# semiflow-core — Math Specification (v0.1.0 + v0.2.0 §9, ADR-0006)

**Audience**: Engineer (Stage 6), QA (Stage 7), Reviewer (Stage 8),
formal-verifier (Stage 5 / Stage 7.5).
**Authority**: This document is normative for the mathematical content of
the v0.1.0 release **and** the v0.2.0 operator-splitting addition (§9).
All formulas are reproduced verbatim from the cited sources. The Engineer
MUST NOT alter signs, coefficients, or shifts.

KaTeX is rendered in rustdoc via `--html-in-header` (DevOps Stage 5).
Display math uses `$$ ... $$`, inline uses `$ ... $`.

---

## 1. Theorem 6 (Remizov 2025) — formula (6)

**Source**: I. D. Remizov, *Vladikavkaz Mathematical Journal* **27**(4), 2025.
DOI [10.46698/a3908-1212-5385-q](https://doi.org/10.46698/a3908-1212-5385-q).
arXiv:2301.06765. Verified verbatim against the published PDF
(`literature-validation.md`, §2.1).

### Statement

Suppose $a, b, c \in UC_b(\mathbb{R})$ are bounded with their derivatives up
to order 3, and there exists a constant $a_0 > 0$ such that
$\inf_{x \in \mathbb{R}} a(x) \ge a_0 > 0$. For each $\varphi \in C_b^\infty(\mathbb{R}) = D(A)$
define

$$
A\varphi(x) \;=\; a(x)\,\varphi''(x) \;+\; b(x)\,\varphi'(x) \;+\; c(x)\,\varphi(x).
$$

For each $t \ge 0$, each $x \in \mathbb{R}$ and each $f \in UC_b(\mathbb{R})$ define

$$
\boxed{\;
(S(t)f)(x) \;=\;
\tfrac{1}{4}\,f\!\left(x + 2\sqrt{a(x)\,t}\right)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,f\!\left(x - 2\sqrt{a(x)\,t}\right)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,f\!\left(x + 2\,b(x)\,t\right)
\;+\; t\,c(x)\,f(x).
\;}\qquad (6)
$$

Then $S$ is a Chernoff function for the $C_0$-semigroup generated by $A$.

**Implementation note (M2)**: $c(x)$ is evaluated *pointwise* in the fourth
term — a single grid node uses $c(x_i)\,f(x_i)$, not $\|c\|_\infty\,f(x_i)$.
For the v0.1.0 heat-Mehler test ($a = 1/2,\ b = c = 0$) this collapses to
zero. The contract preserves the pointwise form for v0.2+ extensions.

### Convergence (Theorem 6, item 3)

For $g$ with bounded derivatives up to order 5,

$$
\left\| \big(S(t/n)\big)^n g \;-\; e^{tA} g \right\|
\;\le\;
\frac{t^2 \, e^{\|c\|\,t}}{n}
\;\cdot\;
\Big( C_0\|g\| + C_1\|g'\| + C_2\|g''\| + C_3\|g'''\| + C_4\|g^{(IV)}\| \Big).
\qquad (9)
$$

The constants $C_0,\dots,C_4$ depend on $\|a\|, \|b\|, \|c\|$ and their
derivatives but not on $g$ or $n$. This bound directly motivates **G3**
(empirical convergence slope $\ge 0.95$).

---

## 2. Chernoff Theorem (Chernoff 1968)

**Source**: P. R. Chernoff, *J. Functional Analysis* **2** (1968) 238–242,
DOI [10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7](https://doi.org/10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7).

Let $F$ be a Banach space and $S \colon [0,\infty) \to L(F)$ strongly
continuous with $S(0) = I$. Suppose $\sup_{t \le T} \|S(t)^k\| \le M e^{\omega k t}$
for some constants $M \ge 1$, $\omega \in \mathbb{R}$. Define the closure of
$S'(0) := \lim_{t \to 0^+}\,(S(t) - I)/t$ on a core $D$ — call it $A$. If
$A$ generates a $C_0$-semigroup $e^{tA}$, then for every $f \in F$ and every
compact $[0, T]$,

$$
\big(S(t/n)\big)^n f \;\xrightarrow[n \to \infty]{}\; e^{tA} f
\qquad \text{strongly, uniformly on } t \in [0, T].
$$

This is the *theoretical justification* for the iteration
`ChernoffSemigroup::evolve(t, f)` in the v0.1.0 contracts.

---

## 3. Quasi-contractivity (G4 invariant)

For `ShiftChernoff1D`, term-by-term inspection of formula (6) gives

$$
\big| (S(\tau) f)(x) \big|
\;\le\;
\big( \tfrac{1}{4} + \tfrac{1}{4} + \tfrac{1}{2} + \tau \,|c(x)| \big)\,\|f\|_\infty
\;=\; \big( 1 + \tau\,|c(x)| \big)\,\|f\|_\infty.
$$

Taking the supremum over $x$ and using $|c(x)| \le \|c\|_\infty$ yields

$$
\boxed{\;
\|S(\tau) f\|_\infty
\;\le\;
\big( 1 + \|c\|_\infty\,\tau \big)\,\|f\|_\infty
\;\le\;
\big( 1 + \|c\|_\infty\,\tau + O(\tau^2) \big)\,\|f\|_\infty.
\;}
$$

The $O(\tau^2)$ slack absorbs interpolation overshoot from the cubic Hermite
adapter; **G4** asserts the explicit bound

$$
\|S(\tau) f\|_\infty \;\le\; \big( 1 + |c|\,\tau + 10\,\tau^2 \big)\,\|f\|_\infty
\quad \text{for } \tau \in (0, 0.1],
$$

over 10000 random proptest cases.

The trait `ChernoffFunction::growth()` returns $(M, \omega) = (1, \|c\|_\infty)$
to record this bound.

---

## 3.5 Boundary policies (v0.2.1, ADR-0007)

`Grid1D::sample(x)` extends the discrete grid function $f \colon \{x_0,\dots,x_{n-1}\} \to \mathbb{R}$
to a continuous function $\widetilde{f} \colon \mathbb{R} \to \mathbb{R}$ via two
adapters: a **boundary policy** (handles $x \notin [x_{\min}, x_{\max}]$) and an
**interpolation kernel** (handles sub-grid $x$ inside the domain). This section
specifies the four boundary policies normatively. The interpolation kernel
(default Catmull-Rom; ADR-0005) operates on indexed control points after the
boundary policy has resolved each requested integer index $j \in \mathbb{Z}$
into either a valid in-range index $i \in [0, n)$ or an extrapolation payload.

Throughout, let $L := x_{\max} - x_{\min}$, $\Delta x := L / (n-1)$, and let
$j \in \mathbb{Z}$ be a (possibly out-of-range) integer index produced by the
interpolation kernel's stencil (e.g., for Catmull-Rom evaluation at $x \in
[x_i, x_{i+1}]$ the four indices are $\{i-1, i, i+1, i+2\}$ and any of them
may fall outside $[0, n)$).

### Index-resolution interface

The internal helper `bc_index(boundary, n, j)` MUST be **total** over
$(\text{BoundaryPolicy}, n \ge 2, j \in \mathbb{Z})$ for v0.2.1 and never
return `Err`. It returns a `BoundaryHit` payload (see
`contracts/semiflow-core.traits.yaml` §4):

- `Inside(i)` — $i \in [0, n)$, value lookup is `values[i]`.
- `OutsideLeft(d)` with $d = -j \ge 1$ — `LinearExtrapolate` only; index
  is $d$ slots to the left of node 0.
- `OutsideRight(d)` with $d = j - (n-1) \ge 1$ — `LinearExtrapolate`
  only; index is $d$ slots to the right of node $n-1$.
- `Zero` — `ZeroExtend` only; the value is exactly $0$.

For `Reflect` and `Periodic` the policy ALWAYS returns `Inside(i)` (any
$j \in \mathbb{Z}$ folds back into $[0, n)$). For `ZeroExtend` the policy
returns `Inside(j as usize)` for $j \in [0, n)$ and `Zero` otherwise. For
`LinearExtrapolate` the policy returns `Inside` in range, else
`OutsideLeft`/`OutsideRight`.

### 3.5.1 `Reflect` (v0.1.0, default)

**Continuous form.** $\widetilde{f}$ is the unique even-extension at both
endpoints:
$$
\widetilde{f}(2 x_{\min} - x) = \widetilde{f}(x), \qquad
\widetilde{f}(2 x_{\max} - x) = \widetilde{f}(x), \qquad x \in \mathbb{R}.
$$
$\widetilde{f}$ is then $2L$-periodic and continuous on $\mathbb{R}$;
piecewise smooth, with corners (kinks in $\widetilde{f}'$) at every
$x_{\min} + k L$, $k \in \mathbb{Z}$, unless $f'(x_{\min}) = f'(x_{\max}) = 0$.
$\widetilde{f}$ is even-reflected, so any odd derivative is anti-symmetric
across the boundary; in particular Neumann-zero data $f'(x_{\min}) = 0$ gives
$\widetilde{f} \in C^1$ near $x_{\min}$.

**Discrete index form.** Period $P = 2(n-1)$. $r := j \bmod P$ via
`rem_euclid` (always $\in [0, P)$). If $r < n$, return $r$; else return
$P - r$ (fold). Returns `Inside(r)` always.

**Cubic-Hermite stability.** The four stencil indices $\{i-1, i, i+1, i+2\}$
near the right boundary fold to $\{n-2, n-1, n-2, n-3\}$ at $i = n-1$; the
control polygon is $(p_{n-2}, p_{n-1}, p_{n-2}, p_{n-3})$ which has zero
discrete derivative at $p_{n-1}$, so Catmull-Rom slope at $x_{\max}$ is
zero. **No oscillation** at the boundary for any input data. This matches
the homogeneous-Neumann boundary condition implicit in the heat-kernel
oracle (§4) — the closed form $u(t,x) = (1+2t)^{-1/2} e^{-x^2/(1+2t)}$ with
domain $[-10, 10]$ has $u'(\pm 10, t) \approx 0$ to machine precision for
all $t \in [0, 1]$, so reflection introduces no oracle bias. **Cross-ref**:
§6.1, §6.2, §9 oracles all use `Reflect`.

### 3.5.2 `ZeroExtend` (v0.1.0)

**Continuous form.**
$$
\widetilde{f}(x) =
\begin{cases}
f(x), & x \in [x_{\min}, x_{\max}], \\
0, & \text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
$$
$\widetilde{f}$ is **discontinuous** at both endpoints unless $f(x_{\min}) =
f(x_{\max}) = 0$. The jump magnitude is $|f(x_{\min})|$ at the left and
$|f(x_{\max})|$ at the right.

**Discrete index form.** If $j \in [0, n)$, return `Inside(j as usize)`;
else return `Zero`. The downstream `bc_value` returns $0.0$ on `Zero`.

**Cubic-Hermite stability.** When the stencil straddles the boundary the
four control points include hard zeros, producing an under-shoot of
magnitude $\sim \tfrac{1}{8}|f(x_{\min/max})|$ over a half-cell width
(Catmull-Rom Lebesgue constant). For data with $|f|$ bounded by $\|f\|_\infty$
this gives $\|\widetilde{f}\|_\infty \le \tfrac{9}{8}\|f\|_\infty$ — a 12.5%
overshoot envelope at the boundary. **Acceptable** for compactly-supported
initial data (e.g., $u_0 = e^{-x^2}$ on $[-10, 10]$ where $u_0(\pm 10) <
2 \times 10^{-44}$). **NOT acceptable** for boundary-active data (e.g.,
constant functions).

### 3.5.3 `Periodic` (v0.2.1, NEW)

**Continuous form.**
$$
\widetilde{f}(x + L) = \widetilde{f}(x), \qquad x \in \mathbb{R}.
$$
Equivalently $\widetilde{f}(x) = f(x_{\min} + ((x - x_{\min}) \bmod L))$.
$\widetilde{f}$ is **continuous on $\mathbb{R}$ iff** $f(x_{\min}) =
f(x_{\max})$; in that case $\widetilde{f} \in C^0(\mathbb{R})$ and is $C^k$
across the seam iff $f^{(j)}(x_{\min}) = f^{(j)}(x_{\max})$ for all $j \le k$.
For generic data the seam introduces a step discontinuity of magnitude
$|f(x_{\max}) - f(x_{\min})|$.

**Discrete index form.** Identify nodes $x_0$ and $x_{n-1}$ as **distinct**
representatives of the period — i.e., the discrete period is exactly $n$
nodes (not $n-1$). The wrap formula is:
$$
r := j \bmod n \in [0, n), \qquad \text{return } \texttt{Inside}(r).
$$
Implemented as `idx.rem_euclid(n as i64) as usize` (Rust's `rem_euclid` for
`i64` always yields a non-negative remainder in $[0, n)$). For derivation
see `.dev-docs/verification/boundary-policies-derivation.md` §2.

**Note** on the $n$ vs $n-1$ choice: this contract uses $n$-node period
(the simple `rem_euclid n` formula). The alternative $L$-period mathematical
identification $f(x_{\min}) \equiv f(x_{\max})$ implicitly demands the user
supplies non-redundant data; if they violate this (different values at
endpoints) the discrete version still wraps correctly at the cost of a
$\Delta x$-scale phase mismatch. Both choices are standard; the simpler
formula wins on suckless grounds.

**Cubic-Hermite stability.** Periodic wrap is fully analogue across the
seam — no boundary stencil collapse. The Catmull-Rom kernel reproduces
periodic smooth functions to $O(\Delta x^4)$. **No oscillation**.
**Required** for: spectral methods, FFT-based convolutions, problems on
the torus $\mathbb{R}/L\mathbb{Z}$.

### 3.5.4 `LinearExtrapolate` (v0.2.1, NEW)

**Continuous form.** Extend $f$ as an affine line on each side using the
one-sided derivative at the boundary:
$$
\widetilde{f}(x) =
\begin{cases}
f(x_{\min}) + (x - x_{\min})\,f'(x_{\min}^+), & x < x_{\min}, \\
f(x), & x_{\min} \le x \le x_{\max}, \\
f(x_{\max}) + (x - x_{\max})\,f'(x_{\max}^-), & x > x_{\max}.
\end{cases}
$$
$\widetilde{f}$ is $C^0$ on $\mathbb{R}$ unconditionally and $C^1$ iff the
boundary derivatives agree with the interior interpolant's slope at the
endpoint.

**Boundary derivative.** Computed from the cubic-Hermite stencil's
left/right one-sided derivative at the endpoint node. For the left
boundary (Catmull-Rom):
$$
f'(x_{\min}^+) \approx \frac{-3 f_0 + 4 f_1 - f_2}{2\,\Delta x}
$$
(second-order forward difference; this is the slope at $s = 0$ of the
Catmull-Rom segment $[x_0, x_1]$ when the stencil's left ghost is taken
to be the symmetric mirror $f_0 - (f_1 - f_0) = 2 f_0 - f_1$, yielding the
above three-point formula). For the right boundary, by symmetry:
$$
f'(x_{\max}^-) \approx \frac{3 f_{n-1} - 4 f_{n-2} + f_{n-3}}{2\,\Delta x}.
$$
Derivation in `.dev-docs/verification/boundary-policies-derivation.md` §3.

**Discrete index form.**
- $j \in [0, n)$: return `Inside(j as usize)`.
- $j < 0$: return `OutsideLeft(d)` with $d := -j \ge 1$. Downstream
  computes $\text{value} := f_0 - d \cdot \Delta x \cdot f'(x_{\min}^+) /
  \Delta x = f_0 - d \cdot \tfrac{-3 f_0 + 4 f_1 - f_2}{2}$
  (i.e., the affine extension evaluated at $j \cdot \Delta x$ left of node 0).
  Equivalently as a closed-form: `value = f_0 + j_signed · slope_left · dx`
  where `j_signed = j` (negative).
- $j \ge n$: return `OutsideRight(d)` with $d := j - (n-1) \ge 1$. Downstream
  computes $\text{value} := f_{n-1} + d \cdot \Delta x \cdot f'(x_{\max}^-)$.

The `bc_value` helper for `LinearExtrapolate` thus consumes the stencil
$\{f_0, f_1, f_2\}$ (left) or $\{f_{n-3}, f_{n-2}, f_{n-1}\}$ (right) plus
the integer offset $d$ to compute the extrapolated value algebraically;
it does NOT recurse through `bc_index`.

**Cubic-Hermite stability — affine-exactness.** For $f(x) = \alpha x +
\beta$ (any affine input), the slope formula evaluates to $\alpha$
**exactly** (machine epsilon), and the extension is exactly the same line
on $\mathbb{R}$. Catmull-Rom on a uniform grid reproduces cubics exactly,
so $\widetilde{f}(x) = \alpha x + \beta$ for all $x \in \mathbb{R}$ with no
floating-point error beyond the f64 round-off in the slope-formula
arithmetic. This is the strongest stability statement among the four
policies and is verified by property `boundary_linear_extrap_affine_exact`
(`contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml`).

**Stability — general data.** For $f \in C^2([x_{\min}, x_{\max}])$ the
extension grows at most linearly in $|x|$:
$\|\widetilde{f}\|_{\infty, [x_{\min} - R, x_{\max} + R]} \le \|f\|_\infty +
R \cdot \|f'\|_{\infty, \text{boundary}}$. This is **unbounded** as
$R \to \infty$ — `LinearExtrapolate` MUST NOT be used for shifts $|s| \gg
\Delta x$ where $f'$ at the boundary is large. The Chernoff shifts in §6
satisfy $|s| \le 2\sqrt{a_{\max} \tau} \le \tfrac{1}{4}$ for $\tau \le 0.1$
and $a \le 5$, well inside the affine-extension's well-conditioned
regime. Document hazard: noisy boundary data ($f$ near the boundary
oscillates at $\Delta x$-scale) amplifies the slope formula by $1/\Delta x$;
ADR-0007 mitigates via test G7 bounding $\|\widetilde{f}\|_\infty$ growth.

### 3.5.5 Cross-references and oracle dependencies

| Oracle / Test               | Boundary policy | Why                                            |
|-----------------------------|-----------------|------------------------------------------------|
| §4 Heat-kernel (G1-leg, G2-leg) | `Reflect`       | Gaussian decays $< 10^{-44}$ at $\pm 10$; reflection bias < machine eps |
| §6.2 Adv-diff (G1, G2, G3-strang) | `Reflect`       | Same Gaussian decay; mass centre stays well inside $[-10, 10]$ at $t = 1$ |
| §9 Strang composition        | `Reflect`       | Inherits inner $D$, $R$ adapters' boundary policy; G3-strang slope test depends on it |
| Periodic stress test (G6, v0.2.1) | `Periodic`     | Sine wave $\sin(2\pi x / L)$ on $[-10, 10]$; verifies `boundary_periodic_round_trip` |
| Affine identity test (G7, v0.2.1) | `LinearExtrapolate` | $f(x) = \alpha x + \beta$ recovered exactly outside grid |

The v0.1.0 / v0.2.0 oracles assume even-reflection symmetry and would
**produce different (worse) results** under `ZeroExtend` (boundary jump
introduces O(1) error in the boundary-strip neighbourhood of width
$\sim 2\sqrt{a t}$) or under `Periodic` (mass leaks through the seam,
violating heat-kernel positivity preservation). The v0.2.1 release adds
new gates G6 and G7 (TBD by QA Stage 7) that exercise `Periodic` and
`LinearExtrapolate` against their respective oracle-data classes.

---

## 4. Heat-kernel oracle (G1, G2)

**Goal**: Solve $\partial_t u = \tfrac{1}{2}\,\partial_{xx} u$ on $\mathbb{R}$
with $u(0, x) = e^{-x^2}$.

**Closed form** (derivation reproduced in `literature-validation.md` §5,
numerically confirmed to machine precision):

$$
\boxed{\;
u(t, x) \;=\; (1 + 2t)^{-1/2}\;\exp\!\left(\frac{-x^2}{1+2t}\right).
\;}
$$

At $t = 1$: $u(1, x) = (3)^{-1/2}\,\exp(-x^2/3)$.

### Terminology note (M1, normative for v0.1.0)

The v0.1.0 PRD called this the *Mehler kernel*. **The correct name is the
heat kernel of the Gaussian initial datum** (the Mehler kernel is the kernel
of the Ornstein–Uhlenbeck semigroup $\partial_t u = \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_{xx} u - x\,\partial_x u$).
All user-facing identifiers, doc strings, and golden-set filenames in
v0.1.0 SHALL use *heat kernel of Gaussian* or *heat oracle*; the legacy
name *Mehler* is permitted only in CHANGELOG.md as a redirect.

Mapping to the v0.1.0 contracts: `ShiftChernoff1D { a: |_| 0.5, b: |_| 0.0, c: |_| 0.0 }`
on the operator $L = \tfrac{1}{2}\,\partial_{xx}$.

---

## 5. Order-1 consistency (`ChernoffFunction::order() == 1`)

Taylor-expand each shift in formula (6) about $\tau = 0$:

$$
f(x \pm 2\sqrt{a\tau})
\;=\;
f(x) \pm 2\sqrt{a\tau}\,f'(x) + 2 a \tau\,f''(x)
\pm \tfrac{4}{3}(a\tau)^{3/2}\,f'''(x) + O(\tau^2),
$$

$$
f(x + 2 b \tau)
\;=\;
f(x) + 2 b \tau\,f'(x) + 2 b^2 \tau^2\,f''(x) + O(\tau^3).
$$

Substituting into (6) and collecting terms (the $\pm$ pairs cancel the
half-integer powers):

$$
S(\tau) f
\;=\;
\Big(\tfrac{1}{4} + \tfrac{1}{4} + \tfrac{1}{2}\Big) f
\;+\; \tau \big( a\,f'' + b\,f' + c\,f \big)
\;+\; O(\tau^2)
\;=\; f \;+\; \tau\,L f \;+\; O(\tau^2).
$$

Therefore $S'(0) f = L f = a f'' + b f' + c f$ on $C^2$, confirming
**consistency order $m = 1$** and justifying `order() -> 1` in the
contract. (The $O(\tau^2)$ remainder controls $C_0,\dots,C_4$ in (9).)

---

## 6. Numerical-method bookkeeping (v0.1.0 and v0.2.0)

### 6.1 v0.1.0 (heat-kernel oracle, plain `ShiftChernoff1D`)

| Symbol      | Meaning                              | v0.1.0 value         |
|-------------|--------------------------------------|----------------------|
| $\Omega$    | Spatial domain                       | $[-10.0,\ 10.0]$     |
| $N$         | Grid nodes                           | $1000$               |
| $\Delta x$  | Grid spacing                         | $20.0 / 999 \approx 0.02$ |
| $a(x)$      | Diffusion coefficient                | $0.5$                |
| $b(x)$      | Drift coefficient                    | $0.0$                |
| $c(x)$      | Reaction coefficient                 | $0.0$                |
| $T$         | Final time                           | $1.0$                |
| $n$         | Chernoff iterations                  | $\{100, 1000\}$ for G1-legacy, G2-legacy |
| $\tau$      | Step size $T/n$                      | $\{0.01, 0.001\}$    |
| $u_0$       | Initial datum                        | $e^{-x^2}$           |
| Boundary    | Out-of-grid policy                   | `Reflect`            |
| Interp      | Sub-grid policy                      | `CubicHermite` (Catmull-Rom) |
| Tolerance G1-legacy | $\|u_{\text{cher}} - u_{\text{oracle}}\|_\infty$ | $< 5 \times 10^{-4}$ |
| Tolerance G2-legacy | same                                  | $< 5 \times 10^{-5}$ |
| Slope G3    | empirical order $\ge 0.95$           |                      |

For the heat-kernel configuration the Chernoff shifts evaluate to
$\pm 2\sqrt{0.5 \cdot \tau} = \pm\sqrt{2\tau}$, which at $\tau = 0.01$ is
$\pm 0.1414\dots$ — about 7 grid nodes wide; well within the cubic-Hermite
stencil's accuracy budget.

### 6.2 v0.2.0 (advection-diffusion oracle, `StrangSplit<DiffusionChernoff, DriftReactionChernoff>`)

ADR-0006 amends the production gates G1, G2, G3-strang to use a
non-trivial drift coefficient so that the operator-splitting Strang test
exercises both `A` and `B`. The closed-form oracle is

$$
\partial_t u \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,\partial_{xx} u \;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,\partial_x u,
\qquad u(0,x) = e^{-x^2},
$$

with closed-form solution (Galilean change of variables $v(t,y) = u(t, y - \beta t)$
reducing to pure heat with $\alpha = 1/2$ — see §9.5 for the derivation):

$$
\boxed{\;
u(t,x) \;=\; (1 + 2t)^{-1/2} \exp\!\Big(-\,\frac{(x + t/2)^2}{1 + 2t}\Big).
\;}
$$

| Symbol      | Meaning                              | v0.2.0 value         |
|-------------|--------------------------------------|----------------------|
| $\Omega$    | Spatial domain                       | $[-10.0,\ 10.0]$     |
| $N$         | Grid nodes (production gates)        | $100000$ (G1, G2, G3-strang) |
| $\Delta x$  | Grid spacing                         | $20.0/99999 \approx 2.0\times 10^{-4}$ |
| $\alpha$    | Diffusion coefficient ($a$)          | $0.5$                |
| $\beta$     | Drift coefficient ($b$)              | $0.5$                |
| $c(x)$      | Reaction coefficient                 | $0.0$                |
| $T$         | Final time                           | $1.0$                |
| $n$         | Chernoff iterations                  | $\{100, 1000\}$ for G1, G2; $\{32, 64, \dots, 1024\}$ for G3-strang |
| $\tau$      | Step size $T/n$                      | $\{0.01, 0.001, \dots\}$ |
| $u_0$       | Initial datum                        | $e^{-x^2}$           |
| Adapter     | Chernoff function                    | `StrangSplit<DiffusionChernoff(α=0.5), DriftReactionChernoff(β=0.5, c=0)>` |
| Boundary    | Out-of-grid policy                   | `Reflect`            |
| Interp      | Sub-grid policy                      | `CubicHermite` (Catmull-Rom) |
| Tolerance G1 | $\|u_{\text{cher}} - u_{\text{oracle}}\|_\infty$ | $< 1 \times 10^{-4}$ |
| Tolerance G2 | same                                  | $< 1 \times 10^{-6}$ |
| Slope G3-strang | empirical order $\ge 1.95$         |                      |
| G4-strang constant | $\|S(\tau) f\|_\infty \le (1 + |c|\tau + 20\tau^2)\|f\|_\infty$ | $\tau \in (0, 0.1]$ |

**Grid-resolution note (2026-04-29 amendment-4, §9.7)**: The production
grid for G1 / G2 / G3-strang is $N = 100000$, revised from the
Amendment-3 value $N = 8000$ after empirical recalibration. Two anchor
measurements (at $N = 1000$ and $N = 8000$) revealed the floor scales as
$\Delta x^{2.32}$, *not* $\Delta x^4$ as Amendment-3 assumed; additionally,
the floor grows linearly in $n$ from per-step cubic-Hermite interp
accumulation when the drift shift $\tau\beta$ falls sub-grid (the
crossover $\tau\beta = \Delta x$ occurs at $n^\star = T\beta/\Delta x$,
which at $N = 8000$ is $n^\star = 200$, well within the slope window
$\{32,\dots,1024\}$). Refining to $N = 100000$ ($\Delta x \approx 2.0\times 10^{-4}$)
drops the floor at $n = 1024$ to $\sim 3.2\times 10^{-10}$, well below the
time error $\sim 2.6\times 10^{-9}$ at the same $n$, restoring the
slope-test sensitivity to the order-2 time integration. Full derivation:
§9.7 below.

`G1-legacy` and `G2-legacy` retain $N = 1000$ (the heat-kernel oracle is
spatially benign at that resolution).

At $t = 1$: $u(1,x) = 3^{-1/2}\,\exp(-(x+0.5)^2 / 3)$. The mass centre
translates from $x = 0$ at $t = 0$ to $x = -0.5$ at $t = 1$, exercising the
$B$ step non-trivially. The `B`-step is exact for these constants
(`(R(\tau) f)(x) = e^{0} f(x + \tau \cdot 0.5) = f(x + \tau/2)`), so all
discretization error is contributed by the $A$-step's local-O($\tau^3$)
truncation, giving the global-O($\tau^2$) signature visible in G3-strang.

---

## 9. Operator splitting `L = A + B` (v0.2.0, ADR-0006)

### 9.1 Decomposition

Split the v0.1.0 operator
$L \varphi(x) = a(x)\varphi''(x) + b(x)\varphi'(x) + c(x)\varphi(x)$ as

$$
A\varphi(x) = a(x)\,\varphi''(x), \qquad
B\varphi(x) = b(x)\,\varphi'(x) + c(x)\,\varphi(x), \qquad
L = A + B.
$$

For constant coefficients (the v0.2.0 acceptance-test oracle, §6.2),
$[A, B] = a\beta\,[\partial_{xx}, \partial_x] + a\,[\partial_{xx}, c\cdot]
= 0 + 0 = 0$, so $e^{tL} = e^{tA}\,e^{tB} = e^{tB}\,e^{tA}$ exactly. For
variable coefficients ($v$0.3.0+) the commutator is non-zero and the
palindromic Strang structure cancels its leading effect (Hairer–Lubich–Wanner,
*Geometric Numerical Integration*, §III.5, Thm 4.1).

#### 9.1.1 Self-adjoint decomposition (v0.3.0, ADR-0008)

For variable `a`, v0.3.0 uses the algebraic identity

$$
A f \;=\; a(x)\,f''(x) \;=\; \partial_x\!\big(a(x)\,\partial_x f\big) \;-\; a'(x)\,\partial_x f
\;=\; A_{\text{self}}\,f \;-\; a'(x)\,f'(x),
$$

where $A_{\text{self}} := \partial_x(a\,\partial_x \cdot)$ is the
**divergence-form self-adjoint generator**. This routes
$A_{\text{self}}$ to `DiffusionChernoff` (which receives both `a`
and `a'` as caller-supplied closures, see §9.2.3 and ADR-0008) and
the residual drift $-a'\,\partial$ into `DriftReactionChernoff` via
the **caller-composed** field
$b_{\text{total}}(x) := b(x) - a'(x)$. The Strang composition

$$
\Phi(\tau) \;=\; D(\tau/2) \;\circ\; R(\tau) \;\circ\; D(\tau/2)
$$

then targets $L = A_{\text{self}} + B_{\text{compensated}}$ where
$B_{\text{compensated}} f := (b - a')\,f' + c\,f$, exactly equivalent
to the original $L = A + B = a\,\partial^2 + b\,\partial + c$.

**Caller responsibility** (v0.3.0 API contract): when constructing
`StrangSplit<DiffusionChernoff, DriftReactionChernoff>` for variable
`a`, the caller MUST construct `R` with $b_{\text{total}} = b - a'$,
**not** the original `b`. Constant-`a` callers (the production case)
have $a' \equiv 0$, so $b_{\text{total}} = b$ trivially — no
behavioural change.

### 9.2 Diffusion Chernoff `D(τ)` — five-point order-2 formula

#### 9.2.1 Constant-`a` derivation (v0.2.0, unchanged)

Chernoff function for $A = a(x)\partial_{xx}$ in the **constant-`a`** baseline:

$$
\boxed{\;
(D(\tau) f)(x) \;=\;
\tfrac{7}{12}\,f(x)
\;+\;\tfrac{3}{16}\,\big[ f(x + 2\sqrt{a(x)\tau}) + f(x - 2\sqrt{a(x)\tau}) \big]
\;+\;\tfrac{1}{48}\,\big[ f(x + 2\sqrt{3 a(x)\tau}) + f(x - 2\sqrt{3 a(x)\tau}) \big].
\;}
$$

**Derivation of the weights $(7/12,\ 3/16,\ 1/48)$**: For constant $a$, take
the Fourier transform. The required symbol is $e^{-a\tau\xi^2}$. Approximate
by $\widehat{D}(\tau,\xi) = w_0 + 2 w_1 \cos(h\xi) + 2 w_2 \cos(H\xi)$ with
shift scales $h = 2\sqrt{a\tau}$ and $H = 2\sqrt{3 a\tau}$. Taylor-expand:

$$
\widehat{D}(\tau,\xi)
= (w_0 + 2 w_1 + 2 w_2)
- (w_1 h^2 + w_2 H^2)\xi^2
+ \tfrac{1}{12}(w_1 h^4 + w_2 H^4)\xi^4
- O(\xi^6).
$$

Match to $e^{-a\tau\xi^2} = 1 - a\tau\,\xi^2 + \tfrac{(a\tau)^2}{2}\xi^4 + O(\xi^6)$:

| Order | Equation                                  |
|-------|-------------------------------------------|
| $\xi^0$ | $w_0 + 2 w_1 + 2 w_2 = 1$               |
| $\xi^2$ | $w_1 h^2 + w_2 H^2 = a\tau$ ⇔ $4 w_1 + 12 w_2 = 1$ |
| $\xi^4$ | $w_1 h^4 + w_2 H^4 = 6(a\tau)^2$ ⇔ $16 w_1 + 144 w_2 = 6$ |

Solving: $w_2 = 1/48$, $w_1 = 3/16$, $w_0 = 7/12$. All weights positive
(probability interpretation valid, sub-Markov kernel) and sum to 1
(confirming $S(0) = I$).

**Leading symbol error.** The first uncancelled Taylor coefficient is at
$\xi^6$: from $\cos(h\xi)$ we get $-h^6/720 \cdot \xi^6$ per cosine, so
the $\xi^6$ coefficient of $\widehat{D}$ is $-\tfrac{1}{360}(w_1 h^6 + w_2 H^6)$.
With $h^6 = 64(a\tau)^3,\ H^6 = 1728(a\tau)^3$, that evaluates to
$-\tfrac{1}{360}\big((3/16)\cdot 64 + (1/48)\cdot 1728\big)(a\tau)^3
= -\tfrac{2}{15}(a\tau)^3$. The exponential symbol $e^{-a\tau\xi^2}$ has
$\xi^6$ coefficient $-\tfrac{(a\tau)^3}{6}$. Difference:
$\widehat{D} - e^{-a\tau\xi^2}\big|_{\xi^6}
= \big(-\tfrac{2}{15} + \tfrac{1}{6}\big)(a\tau)^3
= +\tfrac{1}{30}(a\tau)^3$. So

$$
D(\tau) - e^{\tau A}
\;=\; +\tfrac{1}{30}(a\tau)^3 \cdot \partial_x^6 + O(\tau^4),
$$

i.e., $D(\tau) = e^{\tau A} + O(\tau^3)$ — **local order 2 in time**
(equivalently, $D'(0) = A$ and $D''(0) = A^2$ both match $e^{\tau A}$).

The v0.2.0 implementation `crates/semiflow-core/src/diffusion.rs:162`
evaluates `a` only at the central node `x_i`, which is the correct
choice for constant `a` (every midpoint coincides) but produces an
$O(\tau^2)$ local error for variable `a(x)` because the shift scales
$h_i = 2\sqrt{a(x_i)\tau}$ are systematically biased away from the
true time-integrated diffusion length scale along each segment.

**v9.2.0 recalibration note — G3⁴-2D SPATIAL flagship gate (NORMATIVE).**
The flagship test `spatial_convergence_2d_4th` certifies the *spatial*
order of this K-kernel as a **one-sided floor**: `OLS slope ≤ −3.85`
⇔ `spatial order ≥ ~4`. It is NOT a two-sided "asymptotic slope = −4.0"
equality, and the threshold has never been such (the assertion is `≤`,
not `≈`). The scheme's true asymptotic spatial order is and stays
**exactly 4** (jointly from the ξ⁴-matched weights above and the
cubic-Hermite `f.sample` floor, §9.2.4 mechanism clarification). On the
i7-12700K the discrete f64 temporal floor (~1.2e-9 at n=2000, ~5× the
historically-quoted 2.4e-10) contaminates the fine window
`N∈{400,800,1600}` at n=2000, so the gate is calibrated on the
floor-clean coarse window `N∈{200,300,400}` at `n=4000` (floor ≈0.3e-9
< 3.5% of the smallest spatial error). In that window the measurement is
**pre-asymptotic and super-convergent** — slope ≈ −5.87, ratios
{10.81, 5.40} ABOVE the 4th-order prediction {5.06, 3.16} and DECREASING
toward it (the dx⁶/dx⁸ tail is still active and has not yet been shed).
This is the genuine signature of a ≥4th-order scheme that has not yet
reached the dx⁴ plateau; reaching the plateau cheaply on this HW is
impossible (it needs n≈12000–16000 / ~1hr and re-enters the near-noise
regime). The gate nonetheless discriminates a real order-regression: a
2nd-order degradation gives slope −2.0, which FAILS −3.85 by margin ~1.85.
The test documentation MUST state the true order (4) and the expected
pre-asymptotic coarse-window measurement (≥4, ≈−5.87) in their distinct
roles; it MUST NOT call this window "asymptotic" nor print "Expected ≈
−4.0" as the window's prediction. See ADR-0013 Amendment 3.

#### 9.2.2 Variable-`a` lift (v0.2.3, ADR-0006 Amendment 6.1 — formula β) — SUPERSEDED by §9.2.3

> **STATUS (2026-04-30, end-of-day): SUPERSEDED by §9.2.3 below**
> (ADR-0008, option γ, v0.3.0 API break). The β formula was the
> Stage-5-corrected replacement of α, with the correct generator $A$
> at τ¹ but only local-$O(\tau^2)$ for variable `a` due to the
> symmetric-stencil impossibility theorem. v0.3.0 chooses option γ —
> the API gains an explicit `a'(x)` closure, and the formula is
> restructured as inner-Strang `D = S(τ/2)∘K(τ;a)∘S(τ/2)` (see §9.2.3).
> The β formula below is **NOT shipped** in any released version;
> retained because (1) the symmetric-stencil impossibility theorem in
> this section is canonical mathematical content cited by §9.2.3 and
> ADR-0008, and (2) the Liouville-transform manufactured oracle
> derivation (further below) is reused verbatim by v0.3.0's
> `diffusion_chernoff_variable_gamma_liouville_oracle` property.

> **Architectural history note** (2026-04-30). An earlier candidate
> formula (α, "per-leg midpoint-`a` evaluation") was REJECTED by the
> Stage-5 formal verifier on grounds of τ¹ generator mismatch
> (`.dev-docs/verification/variable-diffusion-midpoint-derivation.md`).
> The asymmetric per-leg shifts $\widetilde h^+ \ne \widetilde h^-$
> generated the symmetrized operator
> $\mathcal{M} f = a(x)\,f''(x) + \tfrac{1}{2}\,a'(x)\,f'(x)$ at τ¹,
> i.e., the wrong PDE. The replacement formula β below restores
> stencil symmetry by sharing one shift between the two wings of each
> pair, recovering Chernoff consistency $D'(0) = A$. Full architect
> re-derivation: `.dev-docs/verification/variable-diffusion-beta-derivation.md`.

For variable `a ∈ C^2(\mathbb{R})$ bounded with bounded derivatives
through order 3 (Theorem 6 hypothesis), the v0.2.3 implementation uses
the **single-pass symmetric arithmetic-mean** lift:

$$
\boxed{\;
\begin{aligned}
h_0(x) &:= 2\sqrt{a(x)\,\tau}, \qquad H_0(x) := 2\sqrt{3\,a(x)\,\tau}, \\[4pt]
\bar{a}_{\text{near}}(x) &:= \tfrac{1}{2}\big[\,a(x + h_0/2) + a(x - h_0/2)\,\big], \\
\bar{a}_{\text{far}}(x)  &:= \tfrac{1}{2}\big[\,a(x + H_0/2) + a(x - H_0/2)\,\big], \\[4pt]
h(x) &:= 2\sqrt{\bar{a}_{\text{near}}(x)\,\tau},
\qquad
H(x) := 2\sqrt{3\,\bar{a}_{\text{far}}(x)\,\tau}, \\[4pt]
(D(\tau) f)(x) &:=
   \tfrac{7}{12}\,f(x)
   + \tfrac{3}{16}\,\big[\,f(x + h) + f(x - h)\,\big]
   + \tfrac{1}{48}\,\big[\,f(x + H) + f(x - H)\,\big].
\end{aligned}
\;}
$$

**Each shift pair is symmetric**: $h^+ = h^- = h$, $H^+ = H^- = H$. The
two arithmetic means $\bar{a}_{\text{near}}, \bar{a}_{\text{far}}$ are
each computed once per node (4 total `a(·)` evaluations: half the
8 of the rejected α formula). The wing weights $(7/12, 3/16, 1/48)$ are
**unchanged** — they remain pinned by the constant-`a` Fourier-symbol
matching of §9.2.1.

**Theorem (v0.2.3 Chernoff consistency, sympy-proven in
`.dev-docs/verification/variable-diffusion-beta-derivation.md` §3.2).**
For $a \in C_b^2(\mathbb{R})$ strictly elliptic and
$f \in C_b^4(\mathbb{R})$,

$$
\big(D(\tau) f\big)(x) \;=\; f(x) \;+\; \tau \cdot a(x)\,f''(x) \;+\; O(\tau^2),
$$

so $D'(0)\,f = A\,f$ — the Chernoff consistency condition holds, and by
Chernoff's product theorem the iterated approximant $(D(T/n))^n f$
converges to $e^{TA} f$ as $n \to \infty$ on a core. **Constant-`a`
reduction**: when $a(x) \equiv a_0$, every $\bar{a}_\bullet = a_0$, so
$h, H$ collapse to the v0.2.2 base scales — the formula is **bit-equal
modulo IEEE arithmetic** to v0.2.2 (≤ 4 ULPs envelope; reduction lemma
below).

**Local order $O(\tau^2)$ for variable `a`** (NOT the speculative
$O(\tau^3)$ targeted by the rejected α formula). The τ² coefficient of
$D(\tau) f - e^{\tau A} f$ at $x = 0$ (sympy-verified, exact rationals):

$$
[\tau^2]\text{ deficit}_\beta(0) \;=\;
\frac{a_0\,(a_2\,f_2 - 4\,a_1\,f_3)}{4}
\;=\; \frac{1}{4}\,a(x)\,a''(x)\,f''(x) \;-\; a(x)\,a'(x)\,f'''(x).
$$

This deficit cannot be eliminated by any choice of $\bar a$ recipe
within the symmetric-stencil family — see the impossibility result
below.

**Theorem (impossibility — symmetric stencil cannot achieve local
$O(\tau^3)$ for variable `a`).** *Let*

$$
D(\tau) f(x) \;=\; w_0\,f(x) \;+\; w_1\,[\,f(x + h) + f(x - h)\,] \;+\; w_2\,[\,f(x + H) + f(x - H)\,]
$$

*with constants $w_k$ and arbitrary $C^\infty$ shift functions $h, H$
of $(\tau, x)$ vanishing at $\tau = 0$. Then for variable
$a \in C_b^2(\mathbb{R})$ with $a' \not\equiv 0$,*

$$
D(\tau) f \;-\; e^{\tau A} f \;\ne\; o(\tau^2)
$$

*in general (the implicit $\tau^2$ coefficient retains a non-removable
$a\,a'\,f'''$ term).*

**Proof sketch.** Symmetric pairs $f(x \pm s) + f(x \mp s) = 2 f + s^2 f'' + (s^4/12) f^{(4)} + \cdots$
contain only **even derivatives** of $f$. Therefore $D(\tau) f$ is a
linear combination of $f, f^{(2)}, f^{(4)}, \ldots$ — odd derivatives
are unreachable. The target

$$
\tfrac{1}{2}\,A^2 f \;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a^2 f^{(4)} \;+\; a\,a'\,f^{(3)} \;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a\,a''\,f^{(2)}
$$

contains $a\,a'\,f^{(3)}$ — an **odd** derivative of $f$. A symmetric
stencil cannot produce $f^{(3)}$ at any order, so the τ² deficit always
retains a non-zero $a\,a'\,f^{(3)}$ contribution whenever $a' \not\equiv 0$.
∎

(Empirically confirmed across **six** $\bar a$ recipes — α per-leg
midpoint, β single-pass mean, β'-Picard 1-iter, trapezoidal 3-point,
Simpson 3-point, central-only — all retain non-zero $a\,a'\,f^{(3)}$ at
τ²; see `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_2_3_variants.py`.)

**Corollary (revised v0.2.3 order claim).**
- **Constant `a`**: $D(\tau) f - e^{\tau A} f = O(\tau^3)$ local;
  global $O(\tau^2)$ via Strang composition (unchanged from §9.2.1).
- **Variable `a ∈ C^2`**: $D(\tau) f - e^{\tau A} f = O(\tau^2)$ local;
  global $O(\tau)$ in iterated $(D(T/n))^n$ approximation.

This is **strictly better** than v0.2.2 in the variable-`a` regime
(v0.2.2's central-only formula was first-order in shift scale, with
its limit semigroup ill-defined for variable `a`; β's limit is the
correct $e^{TA}$). It is **strictly weaker** than the speculative
target (rejected formula α claimed global $O(\tau^2)$ but converged to
the wrong PDE). The order-2 lift for variable `a` is **deferred to
v0.5+** behind an explicit `a'(x)` API or TruncatedExp integrator (see
ADR-0006 Amendment 6.1, §"v0.5+ deferred work").

#### Reduction-to-constant lemma (v0.2.3 regression-safety)

**Claim**: when $a(x) \equiv a_0$ is constant, the v0.2.3 formula β
collapses to the v0.2.2 (≡ v0.2.0) closed form *bit-equal modulo IEEE
arithmetic rearrangement* (≤ 4 ULPs envelope).

- For constant $a \equiv a_0$, every $a(x \pm h_0/2) = a_0$ and
  $a(x \pm H_0/2) = a_0$, so the symmetric arithmetic means
  $\bar{a}_{\text{near}} = (a_0 + a_0)/2 = a_0$ and
  $\bar{a}_{\text{far}} = a_0$ — exact in IEEE-754 (sum of two identical
  values divided by 2 is bit-exact).
- Lifted shifts $h = 2\sqrt{a_0 \tau}$, $H = 2\sqrt{3 a_0 \tau}$ —
  identical to v0.2.2's central-node base scales.
- The four `f.sample(x \pm h)` and `f.sample(x \pm H)` calls receive
  bit-equal arguments to v0.2.2 (same `2.0 * libm::sqrt(a_0 * tau)`,
  same `2.0 * libm::sqrt(3.0 * a_0 * tau)`).
- The weights $(7/12, 3/16, 1/48)$ are loaded from the same constants
  `W0, W1, W2` and applied in the same order. The final reduction
  $W_0 \cdot f[i] + W_1 \cdot (f(x+h) + f(x-h)) + W_2 \cdot (f(x+H) + f(x-H))$
  is IEEE-bit-equal modulo at most ≤ 4 ULPs (the two extra `a(·) + a(·)`
  adds and one `* 0.5` per pair contribute ≤ 1 ULP each, with the inputs
  numerically identical so the sums are exact).

**Consequence**: the v0.2.0/v0.2.1/v0.2.2 acceptance gates G1, G2,
G3-strang, G4-strang (all use constant $\alpha = 0.5$) are **unchanged
to within floating-point rearrangement noise** (bounded by ≤ 4 ULPs per
evaluation; well below the gate thresholds $1\!\times\!10^{-4}$,
$1\!\times\!10^{-6}$, slope tolerance $0.05$). G1-legacy / G2-legacy
(plain `ShiftChernoff1D`, no `DiffusionChernoff` involvement) are
unaffected. **The v0.2.3 upgrade is regression-safe by construction.**
Property `diffusion_chernoff_constant_fast_path_exact`
(properties.yaml) enforces this empirically over 1000 random
$(a_0, \tau)$ pairs to tolerance $1\!\times\!10^{-13}$.

#### Variable-`a` oracle (Liouville-transform manufactured solution)

The Stage-5 verifier identified a critical test-design gap in the
original v0.2.3 plan: **Richardson self-consistency cannot detect
generator mismatch**. A self-consistent discretization of the *wrong*
PDE will pass any slope-against-its-own-reference gate. The verification
of formula β therefore mandates a **closed-form variable-`a` oracle**.

**Profile** (architect re-design, sympy-verified):

$$
\boxed{\;
a(x) \;:=\; (1 + \gamma x)^2,
\qquad x > -\tfrac{1}{\gamma},\ \gamma > 0,
\;}
$$

is $C^\infty$ on its domain, strictly positive, with bounded derivatives
of all orders on any compact interval $[x_{\min}, x_{\max}]$ separated
from $x = -1/\gamma$ — satisfying Theorem 6 hypotheses uniformly on
finite-grid domains.

**Liouville transform** $y(x) := \int dx/\sqrt{a(x)} = \ln(1 + \gamma x)/\gamma$
with $\varphi(x) := a(x)^{-1/4} = (1 + \gamma x)^{-1/2}$ and
$v(t, y) := \varphi(x(y))\,u(t, x(y))$ where $x(y) = (e^{\gamma y} - 1)/\gamma$.
Sympy direct verification (`/tmp/verify_liouville_oracle.py`,
preserved at `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_liouville_oracle.py`)
confirms the transformed PDE:

$$
\boxed{\;
v_t(t, y) \;=\; v_{yy}(t, y) \;-\; \tfrac{\gamma^2}{4}\,v(t, y)
\;}
$$

with the Schrödinger-like potential $V \equiv -\gamma^2/4$ being **constant**
(NOT a Pöschl-Teller or other position-dependent potential).

**Closed-form oracle.** Substitute $v(t, y) = e^{-\gamma^2 t / 4}\,w(t, y)$.
Then $w$ satisfies the **pure heat equation in $y$**:

$$
w_t \;=\; w_{yy}, \qquad w(0, y) \;=\; \varphi(x(y))\,f(x(y))
\;=\; (1 + \gamma\,x(y))^{-1/2}\,f(x(y))
\;=\; e^{-\gamma y/2}\,f\!\big((e^{\gamma y} - 1)/\gamma\big).
$$

Closed-form heat-kernel solution:

$$
w(t, y) \;=\; \int_{-\infty}^{\infty} \frac{1}{\sqrt{4\pi t}}\,
e^{-(y - y')^2/(4 t)}\;w(0, y')\,dy'.
$$

**Reverse-transform**:

$$
\boxed{\;
u(t, x) \;=\; \varphi(x)^{-1}\,e^{-\gamma^2 t / 4}\,w(t, y(x))
\;=\; (1 + \gamma x)^{1/2}\,e^{-\gamma^2 t / 4}\,w\big(t,\,\ln(1 + \gamma x)/\gamma\big).
\;}
$$

For Gaussian initial data $f(x) = e^{-x^2/(2 \sigma^2)}$, the integral
defining $w(t, y)$ is **not elementary** but reduces to a smooth, unimodal,
exponentially decaying one-dimensional integrand evaluable to
$\approx 10^{-12}$ relative precision by `scipy.integrate.quad` (or
analogous high-precision quadrature in Rust via `pyo3` bridge in
test-only `[dev-dependencies]`). **This is the closed-form oracle**.

The QA gate `diffusion_chernoff_variable_order1_liouville_oracle`
(properties.yaml, replacing the rejected
`diffusion_chernoff_variable_order2`) compares $(D_\beta(T/n))^n f$
against this closed-form solution. **Asserted**: log-log slope of error
vs. $\tau = T/n$ is $\le -0.95$ over the 5-point sweep
$n \in \{32, 64, 128, 256, 512\}$, confirming β's theoretical global
$O(\tau)$ for variable `a`. A future v0.5+ implementation using an
explicit `a'(x)` API (option γ) or TruncatedExp integrator would
**automatically** be detected by this gate as slope $\le -1.95$,
empirically validating the order-2 lift.

This oracle is **stronger than the rejected Richardson self-consistency
gate** in three respects:

1. **Correctness**: detects generator mismatch (formula α would FAIL
   here despite passing Richardson self-consistency, because α
   converges to $e^{T\mathcal{M}}$ while the oracle evaluates $e^{TA}$).
2. **Order**: distinguishes global $O(\tau)$ (β) from global $O(\tau^2)$
   (hypothetical v0.5+) — the slope gate $\le -0.95$ passes for β,
   $\le -1.95$ would pass for v0.5+.
3. **Reproducibility**: the closed-form oracle is *deterministic* (no
   stochastic Monte Carlo, no spectral truncation parameters). The
   `scipy.integrate.quad` adaptive integrator is well-conditioned for
   this smooth integrand.

(Reference for symmetric-stencil impossibility: §9.2.2 above. Reference
for Liouville transform of variable-coefficient parabolic PDEs:
Olver, *Asymptotics and Special Functions*, 1974, §5.2; Polyanin
& Zaitsev, *Handbook of Linear PDEs*, 2nd ed. 2016, §1.1.

#### 9.2.3 Variable-`a` lift (v0.3.0, ADR-0008 — option ζ, true order-2 via `a, a', a''`) ✅ ADOPTED

**Status**: ADOPTED for v0.3.0 release (ζ-A formula, ADR-0008 Amendment 1).
The γ-A formula (preserved below as the **structural baseline**) is
extended with an explicit τ²-correction polynomial in `a, a', a''`
that kills the γ-A τ²-deficit exactly. Sympy-verified at
`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_3_0_zeta.py` (reproducible;
exit 0 on success — gates Z_τ⁰, Z_τ¹, **Z_τ² (NEW, NORMATIVE)**,
Z_const-a all pass). The γ-A baseline gates are preserved at
`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_3_0_gamma.py` and document
the deficit polynomial that ζ-A kills.

##### 9.2.3.A γ-A baseline (preserved verbatim — structural skeleton)

**Decomposition identity** (algebraic):

$$
A f \;=\; a(x)\,f''(x) \;=\; \partial_x\!\big(a(x)\,\partial_x f\big) \;-\; a'(x)\,\partial_x f
\;=\; A_{\text{self}} f \;-\; a'(x)\,f'(x),
$$

where $A_{\text{self}} := \partial_x(a\,\partial_x \cdot)$ is the
**divergence-form self-adjoint** generator. v0.3.0 routes
$A_{\text{self}}$ to `DiffusionChernoff` and the residual $-a'\partial$
to `DriftReactionChernoff` via caller-composed
$b_{\text{total}} := b - a'$. The Strang composition

$$
\Phi(\tau) \;=\; D(\tau/2) \;\circ\; R(\tau) \;\circ\; D(\tau/2)
$$

then targets $L = A + B = A_{\text{self}} + B_{\text{compensated}}$
where $B_{\text{compensated}} f := (b - a')\,f' + c\,f$.

**Inner-Strang formula for $D(\tau)$** (the v0.3.0 "γ-FINAL-v5" formula):

$$
\boxed{\;
\begin{aligned}
D(\tau) \;&:=\; S(\tau/2) \;\circ\; K(\tau;\,a) \;\circ\; S(\tau/2),\\[6pt]
\bigl(S(s)\,g\bigr)(x) \;&:=\; g\bigl(x + s\,a'(x)\bigr) \qquad \text{(pure-drift exponential)},\\[6pt]
\bigl(K(\tau;a)\,g\bigr)(x) \;&:=\;
   \tfrac{7}{12}\,g(x)
   \;+\;\tfrac{3}{16}\,\big[g(x + h_0) + g(x - h_0)\big]
   \;+\;\tfrac{1}{48}\,\big[g(x + H_0) + g(x - H_0)\big],\\[4pt]
h_0(x) \;&:=\; 2\sqrt{a(x)\,\tau}, \qquad H_0(x) := 2\sqrt{3\,a(x)\,\tau}.
\end{aligned}
\;}
$$

The weights $(7/12,\,3/16,\,1/48)$ are **unchanged** from §9.2.1 — they
are pinned by the constant-`a` Fourier-symbol matching and remain the
unique solution of the 3-equation linear system that produces local
$O(\tau^3)$ for constant `a`.

**Mathematical interpretation** ($A_{\text{self}}$ as sum of two
operators).
$$
A_{\text{self}} \;=\; a\,\partial_x^2 \;+\; a'\,\partial_x.
$$
The inner-Strang $S(\tau/2) \circ K(\tau;a) \circ S(\tau/2)$ is the
palindromic Strang split of $A_{\text{self}}$ as the sum of the
diffusion operator $a\,\partial^2$ (handled by the symmetric 5-point
$K$-factor) and the drift field $a'\,\partial$ (handled by the
exact pure-drift exponential $S(s) = \exp(s\,a'\,\partial)$).

**Theorem (v0.3.0 Chernoff τ¹ consistency)**. For
$a \in C_b^2(\mathbb R)$ strictly elliptic and
$f \in C_b^4(\mathbb R)$:

$$
\bigl(D(\tau)\,f\bigr)(x) \;=\; f(x) \;+\; \tau\,\bigl(A_{\text{self}}\,f\bigr)(x) \;+\; O(\tau^2),
$$

so $D'(0)\,f = A_{\text{self}}\,f$ exactly (sympy-proven at $x = 0$ in
`verify_v0_3_0_gamma.py`, gate **G_τ¹**, deficit algebraically zero).
By Chernoff's product theorem (Engel-Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups*,
Ch. II), the iterated approximant $(D(T/n))^n f \to e^{T A_{\text{self}}} f$
as $n \to \infty$ on a core. Composed with $R$ via Strang on the
caller's $b_{\text{total}} = b - a'$, the full PDE limit is
$e^{TL}f$ where $L = a\,\partial^2 + b\,\partial + c$ — **the correct
target operator**.

**Sympy gate G_const (constant-`a` regression)**. When $a' \equiv 0$,
$S(s)g(x) = g(x + 0) = g(x)$ — the identity. Therefore
$D(\tau) = K(\tau; a_0) \equiv$ v0.2.2 5-point central-`a` formula
**exactly** (algebraically; sympy verifies $D - D_{v0.2.2} = 0$
identically in $f_0, \ldots, f_6$). G1, G2, G3-strang, G4-strang
acceptance gates pass **bit-equal** for the constant-`α=0.5`
production oracle.

**Theorem (v0.3.0 local-order ceiling)**. The full local order is
$O(\tau^2)$ for variable `a`, **not** $O(\tau^3)$, because:

$$
[\tau^2]\bigl(D(\tau)f - e^{\tau A_{\text{self}}}f\bigr)(0) \;=\;
-a_0\,a_1\,f_3 \;-\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a_0\,a_2\,f_2 \;-\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,a_1\,a_2\,f_1.
$$

The $-a_0\,a_1\,f_3$ term — the same odd-derivative obstruction as in
§9.2.2 — is **structural**: any composition of pure-drift translation
$S(s)$ with a symmetric K-factor produces the structure
$S(\tau/2)[K[S(\tau/2)f]]$ whose $\tau^2$ Taylor coefficient cannot
fully reproduce $A_{\text{self}}^2/2 = (a\partial^2 + a'\partial)^2/2$
without explicit knowledge of $a''(x)$ (which the v0.3.0 API does not
carry). The remaining $-a_0 a_2 f_2/2 - a_1 a_2 f_1/4$ residue
involves $a''$ explicitly. Sympy gate **G_τ²** is informational
(non-zero); the normative gates are **G_τ⁰**, **G_τ¹**, **G_const**.

The order ceiling for variable `a` therefore remains:

| Regime | Local order ($D$) | Global order (Strang $\Phi$) | Generator |
|--------|-------------------|------------------------------|-----------|
| Constant `a` | $O(\tau^3)$ exact | $O(\tau^2)$ via Strang | $A$ ✓ |
| Variable `a ∈ C^2$ | $O(\tau^2)$ | $O(\tau)$ | $A_{\text{self}} \;\Rightarrow\; e^{TL}f$ via R-compensation ✓ |

**This is the SAME convergence rate as the rejected β formula
(§9.2.2)**. The architectural value of γ over β is **not** order
improvement — both are blocked by the same impossibility theorem —
but rather:

1. **Mathematical rigor**: $D(\tau)$ corresponds to the exact
   divergence-form generator $A_{\text{self}}$; v0.2.2 silent
   degradation is gone.
2. **API surface change** that unlocks future order-2 lifts (TruncatedExp
   integrator in v0.4.0, $a''(x)$ input in v0.5.0) without further
   breaking changes.
3. **R reuse**: v0.2.2 RK2 `DriftReactionChernoff` is reused
   verbatim with the caller-composed $b_{\text{total}} = b - a'$.

**Performance**. Per-node cost: 1 central `a(x)`, 2 `a_prime(x)`
(at $x$ and $x + a'(x)\,\tau/2$), 4 `f.sample` (after the inner-
Strang's S-shifted positions), 2 `libm::sqrt`, 1 `validate_a_x`. This
is +2 `fn(f64)→f64` calls vs v0.2.2 (estimated +5-10 ns/node;
v0.2.2 baseline ~150 ns/node; predicted overhead 3-7%, within ±5%
target).

**Engineer pseudocode** (from `traits.yaml` `DiffusionChernoff.apply.semantics`):

```rust
// v0.3.0 γ-A inner-Strang: D(τ) = S(τ/2) ∘ K(τ;a) ∘ S(τ/2)
let x      = self.grid.x_at(i);
// S(τ/2) inner: shift each evaluation point of K back by (τ/2)·a'(...)
// Implementation routes the composition pointwise:
//   For target output position x_i, we want
//     D(τ)f(x_i) = (S∘K∘S)(f)(x_i)
//                = (S∘K)(f)(x_i + (τ/2)·a'(x_i))
//                = K[ S(τ/2)f ](x_pre)         where x_pre := x_i + (τ/2)·a'(x_i)
//                = w₀·(Sf)(x_pre)
//                + w₁·[(Sf)(x_pre + h₀) + (Sf)(x_pre − h₀)]
//                + w₂·[(Sf)(x_pre + H₀) + (Sf)(x_pre − H₀)]
//   with h₀ = 2·√(a(x_pre)·τ),  H₀ = 2·√(3·a(x_pre)·τ).
//   Then (Sf)(y) = f(y + (τ/2)·a'(y))   — additional inner shift per K-arm.

let s_half     = 0.5 * tau;
let dx_pre     = s_half * (self.a_prime)(x);              // S(τ/2) outer-right shift
let x_pre      = x + dx_pre;                              // K-factor evaluation centre
let a_at_pre   = (self.a)(x_pre);
validate_a_x(a_at_pre, x_pre)?;
let h0         = 2.0 * libm::sqrt(a_at_pre * tau);
let H0         = 2.0 * libm::sqrt(3.0 * a_at_pre * tau);

// 5-point K, with S(τ/2) inner shift on each f.sample:
let center_pos = x_pre + s_half * (self.a_prime)(x_pre);  // (Sf)(x_pre)
let near_p_pos = x_pre + h0;
let near_p_pos = near_p_pos + s_half * (self.a_prime)(near_p_pos);
let near_n_pos = x_pre - h0;
let near_n_pos = near_n_pos + s_half * (self.a_prime)(near_n_pos);
let far_p_pos  = x_pre + H0;
let far_p_pos  = far_p_pos + s_half * (self.a_prime)(far_p_pos);
let far_n_pos  = x_pre - H0;
let far_n_pos  = far_n_pos + s_half * (self.a_prime)(far_n_pos);

let center     = W0 * f.sample(center_pos)?;
let near       = W1 * (f.sample(near_p_pos)? + f.sample(near_n_pos)?);
let far        = W2 * (f.sample(far_p_pos)?  + f.sample(far_n_pos)?);
result.values[i] = center + near + far;
```

Total: ~30 lines (under 50-line cap); `diffusion.rs` total ≈ 220
(under 500-line file cap; +20 LOC vs v0.2.2 for the extra
`a_prime` field, S-factor shifts, and updated docstrings).

**Constant-`a` fast path**. When `a_prime` is the literal `|_| 0.0`,
`dx_pre = 0`, `x_pre = x`, all four S-inner shifts are 0, and the
five `f.sample` arguments collapse to v0.2.2's `(x, x±h₀, x±H₀)`.
The Rust optimizer **should** constant-fold the `S` operations away
when `a_prime` is the literal zero closure. Engineer Stage 6 verifies
this via `cargo bench --bench heat_1d` (target: ±2% vs v0.2.2 for
constant α=0.5; ±5% otherwise).

**Reduction-to-constant lemma (γ regression-safety, sympy-proven)**.
For `a' ≡ 0`, $S(s)$ is the identity for all $s \in [0, \tau]$, so
$D(\tau) = K(\tau; a_0)$ — the v0.2.2 central-$a$ 5-point formula
exactly. Algebraically $D_\gamma|_{a'\equiv 0} - D_{v0.2.2} = 0$ in
the polynomial ring (sympy gate **G_const**). Tolerance for the
production property `diffusion_chernoff_constant_fast_path_exact`
is `1e-13` over 1000 random `(a_0, τ)` pairs — passes by algebraic
identity (worst-case ≤ 4 ULPs from any small floating-point
rearrangement that the optimizer might introduce).

**Forward-compatibility** (v0.4.0+ deferred work):
- **v0.4.0 (option ε, TruncatedExp)**: replace inner-Strang with
  $\exp(\tau \cdot \overline{A_{\text{self}}})$ where
  $\overline{A_{\text{self}}}$ is the time-averaged generator over
  $[0, \tau]$. Lifts to local-$O(\tau^3)$ / global-$O(\tau^2)$ for
  variable `a`. Reuses $(a, a')$ interface verbatim.
- **v0.5.0 (option ζ, $a''$ input)**: add `a_double_prime: fn(f64) -> f64`
  field; explicit higher-order Taylor corrections kill the residual
  $-a\,a''\,f''/2 - a'\,a''\,f'/4$ terms. Lifts to local-$O(\tau^4)$
  / global-$O(\tau^3)$. SemVer minor break (third closure on the
  struct), but mentally budgeted as part of the v0.3.0 architectural
  trajectory.
- **v0.6.0+** (resolvent quadrature): $R_\lambda f = \sum_k w_k S(\tau_k)f$
  reuses $(a, a')$ verbatim; no further API change.

##### 9.2.3.B ζ-A extension (TRUE order-2 lift, NORMATIVE for v0.3.0 release)

**Status**: NORMATIVE. The shipping v0.3.0 formula is **ζ-A** — γ-A
inner-Strang plus an explicit τ²-correction polynomial in
`(a, a', a'', f', f'', f''')`. The γ-A baseline (§9.2.3.A) is the
structural skeleton; ζ-A adds a single closed-form correction term
that kills the γ-A τ²-deficit exactly (sympy-proven, gate **Z_τ²**,
NEW, NORMATIVE, in
`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_3_0_zeta.py`).

**Sympy-proven τ²-deficit of γ-A** (reproduced from §9.2.3.A above):

$$
[\tau^2]\bigl(D_{\gamma\text{-A}}(\tau)f - e^{\tau A_{\text{self}}}f\bigr)(x)
\;=\; -\,a(x)\,a'(x)\,f'''(x) \;-\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a(x)\,a''(x)\,f''(x)
                              \;-\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,a'(x)\,a''(x)\,f'(x).
$$

**ζ-A formula** (γ-A baseline + the negative of the deficit, evaluated
pointwise):

$$
\boxed{\;
\begin{aligned}
D_\zeta(\tau)\,f(x) \;:=\;\; & D_{\gamma\text{-A}}(\tau)\,f(x) \\
\;+\;\; & \tau^2 \cdot \Bigl[\,a(x)\,a'(x)\,f'''(x) \;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a(x)\,a''(x)\,f''(x) \;+\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,a'(x)\,a''(x)\,f'(x)\,\Bigr].
\end{aligned}
\;}
$$

The bracketed correction term is **non-symmetric in `f`-derivatives**
(it mixes `f'`, `f''`, and `f'''`) — this is the structural reason ζ-A
escapes the symmetric-K-factor impossibility theorem of §9.2.2: the
correction is added OUTSIDE the K-factor, contributing `f`-Taylor
coefficients of all parities directly. The price is one new caller
input — the analytic `a''(x)`, supplied as a third `fn(f64) -> f64`
closure on `DiffusionChernoff`.

**Algebraic identity (sympy gate Z_τ², NORMATIVE)**: Expanding
$D_\zeta(\tau)f(x)$ to $O(\tau^3)$ in the polynomial-Taylor model
`a(x) = a₀ + a₁x + (a₂/2)x² + (a₃/6)x³`,
`f(x) = Σ fₖ·xᵏ/k!` (so `aₖ = a^(k)(0)`, `fₖ = f^(k)(0)`) at $x = 0$:

```text
τ⁰ coefficient   = f0
target           = f0
Z_τ⁰  identity? True

τ¹ coefficient   = a0·f2 + a1·f1
target A_self f  = a0·f2 + a1·f1
Z_τ¹  Chernoff consistency? True

τ² coefficient   = a0²·f4/2 + 2·a0·a1·f3 + 3·a0·a2·f2/2 + a0·a3·f1/2
                 + a1²·f2 + a1·a2·f1/2
target A²f / 2   = a0²·f4/2 + 2·a0·a1·f3 + 3·a0·a2·f2/2 + a0·a3·f1/2
                 + a1²·f2 + a1·a2·f1/2
τ² deficit       = 0
Z_τ²  TRUE order-2 lift? True   [NORMATIVE — NEW IN ζ]

Constant-a regression: D_ζ − D_v022 = 0
Z_const-a  bit-equal? True       [NORMATIVE]
```

The τ³ residual is bounded — a polynomial in `a₀,…,a₃, f₁,…,f₆` that
vanishes for constant `a` (where `a₁ = a₂ = a₃ = 0`) and is finite
for `a ∈ C³(ℝ)` strictly elliptic with `f ∈ C⁵(ℝ)` Schwartz-class.
See `verify_v0_3_0_zeta.py` for the exact τ³ form.

**Constant-`a` reduction lemma (gate Z_const-a, NORMATIVE)**. When
`a' ≡ 0 ∧ a'' ≡ 0`, the bracketed correction
`a·a'·f''' + ½·a·a''·f'' + ¼·a'·a''·f'` collapses to
`a·0·f''' + ½·a·0·f'' + ¼·0·0·f' = 0` identically, AND the γ-A
baseline collapses to v0.2.2 by §9.2.3.A's reduction lemma. Therefore
$D_\zeta = D_{\gamma\text{-A}} = K = D_{v0.2.2}$ exactly (algebraically;
sympy verifies $D_\zeta - D_{v0.2.2} = 0$ identically). Bit-equal output
to v0.2.2 is preserved for all current call sites (10 sites, all
constant `α = 0.5`).

**Order claim (revised, honest — Amendment 2, 2026-04-30)**:

After Stage 7 QA measured Richardson slope $\approx -1$ for variable `a`
(γ = 0.1 Liouville oracle) instead of the predicted $-2$, formal verifier
investigation (`.dev-docs/reports/ZETA_EMPIRICAL_INVESTIGATION.md`,
2026-04-30) decomposed the discrepancy into five hypotheses (H1-H5) and
isolated the cause as **H1: numerical-derivative discretization noise**.
H4 (implementation bug) and H5 (theoretical limit / impossibility-theorem
analogue for ζ-A) are REJECTED. H1 is ACCEPTED:

- **Mathematical (operator algebra)**: ζ-A is local $O(\tau^3)$ for
  $a \in C^3(\mathbb R)$. Sympy gates `Z_τ⁰`, `Z_τ¹`, `Z_τ²`,
  `Z_const-a` all pass; multi-`τ` ratios with **analytic** samples
  (no FD) converge cleanly to $8$ (cubic), confirming the formula.
- **Implementation ceiling**: the τ²-correction uses cubic-spline
  `f.sample()` at off-grid positions plus 5-point central FD for
  `f', f'', f'''` with stencil step `Δ = max(2·dx, √τ)`. Empirical
  per-step sup-norm error from spline + FD is $O(\tau^2)$ (4× ratio
  per τ-halving, verified with γ = 0.1 Liouville oracle), accumulating
  over `n` steps to **global $O(\tau^1)$ for variable `a`** — the same
  rate as v0.2.2 `ShiftChernoff1D` for variable coefficients.
- **Constant `a`** (`a' ≡ 0 ∧ a'' ≡ 0`): the correction polynomial
  vanishes identically and γ-A reduces to v0.2.2 `K`-only (gate
  Z_const-a). The single-operator iterate retains **global
  $O(\tau^2)$** because the per-step `O(\tau^3)$` truncation has
  no FD-driven floor (analytic samples + symmetric 5-point stencil
  with constant `a` is exact local $O(\tau^3)$). The γ = 0 sub-test
  empirically confirms slope $-2$ — definitive proof that
  single-operator Chernoff iteration **CAN** achieve global $O(\tau^2)$;
  the obstruction for variable `a` is purely numerical, not theoretical.
- **What ζ-A delivers for variable `a` in v0.3.0** despite the global
  $O(\tau^1)$ implementation rate:
  1. **Correct generator** $A_{\text{self}} = \partial(a \cdot \partial)$
     (divergence-form, mathematically rigorous parabolic operator);
  2. **~1000× tighter constant** in the per-step error envelope
     (factor of $10^{-3}$ reduction in absolute error at production
     grids, vs the γ-A baseline without τ²-correction);
  3. **Bit-equal v0.2.2 regression-safety** for constant-`a` callers
     (gate Z_const-a, sympy-proven algebraic identity);
  4. **Forward-compatible API surface** for v0.4.0 TruncatedExp integrator
     (option ε), which avoids FD on `f`-derivatives entirely and
     therefore breaks the implementation ceiling.

**Implementation order claim (final, honest)**:

| Regime | Local order ($D$, math) | Global order (impl, Chernoff iterate) | Strang composition (full PDE) | Generator |
|--------|-------------------------|---------------------------------------|-------------------------------|-----------|
| Constant `a`                    | $O(\tau^3)$ exact     | $O(\tau^2)$ (no FD floor — bit-equal v0.2.2)  | $O(\tau^2)$ via Strang          | $A$ ✓ |
| Variable `a \in C^3(\mathbb R)` | $O(\tau^3)$ (sympy ✓) | **$O(\tau^1)$** (FD discretization ceiling)   | $O(\tau^1)$ (limited by D)      | $A_{\text{self}}$ ✓ (divergence form) |
| Variable `a, b, c` (full)       | $O(\tau^2)$ (limited by R) | $O(\tau^1)$ (limited by D variable-a)    | $O(\tau^1)$                     | $L = A_{\text{self}} + B_{\text{compensated}}$ ✓ |

**True global $O(\tau^2)$ for variable `a` is DEFERRED to v0.4.0**
(TruncatedExp integrator, option ε), which does not require FD on
`f`-derivatives. v0.3.0 ζ-A is **necessary forward-compatibility
groundwork**: the same 5-arg `(a, a', a'', a_norm, grid)` API surface
will be reused by v0.4.0 TruncatedExp, which adds a NEW type alongside
`DiffusionChernoff` (no further breaking changes). v0.3.0 ships
because: (1) the correct generator matters for theoretical correctness
even at $O(\tau^1)$, (2) the 1000× constant tightening directly
benefits production, (3) constant-`a` regression-safety is bit-equal,
and (4) the API break is needed once and only once. See ADR-0008
Amendment 2 for the full reconciliation.

**Numerical-derivative stencil specification (5-point central FD)**.
The pointwise τ² correction
`a·a'·f''' + ½·a·a''·f'' + ¼·a'·a''·f'` is exact in operator algebra,
but the implementation must compute `f', f'', f'''` numerically from
grid samples. The recommended stencil is **central finite differences
with step `Δ` chosen** such that

$$
\boxed{\;\Delta \;=\; \max\!\bigl(2\,\mathrm{dx},\;\sqrt{\tau}\bigr)\;}
$$

where `dx = self.grid.dx()`. Pointwise:

$$
\begin{aligned}
f'(x)   \;&\approx\; \frac{f(x+\Delta) - f(x-\Delta)}{2\,\Delta}                                          \;+\; O(\Delta^2),\\[4pt]
f''(x)  \;&\approx\; \frac{f(x+\Delta) - 2\,f(x) + f(x-\Delta)}{\Delta^2}                                  \;+\; O(\Delta^2),\\[4pt]
f'''(x) \;&\approx\; \frac{f(x+2\Delta) - 2\,f(x+\Delta) + 2\,f(x-\Delta) - f(x-2\Delta)}{2\,\Delta^3}     \;+\; O(\Delta^2).
\end{aligned}
$$

**Algebraic justification of `Δ` choice**. The leading correction
term is $\tau^2 \cdot \text{[stencil-approximated derivatives]}$.
Stencil truncation is $O(\Delta^2 \cdot f^{(5)})$. The total
τ-residual contribution of the correction is therefore
$\tau^2 \cdot O(\Delta^2)$, which must remain $\leq O(\tau^3)$
(within the local-$O(\tau^3)$ budget). This requires
$\Delta^2 \leq O(\tau)$, i.e., $\Delta \leq \sqrt{\tau}$.

For very small `τ` (≤ `dx²`), $\sqrt{\tau}$ becomes sub-grid-spacing
and the stencil samples `f` at very nearby points — floating-point
cancellation in $(f(x+\Delta) - f(x-\Delta))/(2\Delta)$ becomes
significant. The floor `Δ ≥ 2·dx` ensures the stencil always spans
**≥ 4 grid cells** (the `f'''` stencil reaches `x ± 2Δ`, requiring
`4·dx` span). This is well-resolved by the cubic Hermite interpolant
on the v0.1.0 grid (`N ≥ 4` by `Grid1D::new` precondition).

The choice $\Delta = \max(2\,\mathrm{dx}, \sqrt{\tau})$ balances:
- **τ-residual control**: $\Delta = \sqrt{\tau}$ ⇒ stencil error
  $O(\tau)$ ⇒ correction error $O(\tau^3)$, within budget.
- **floating-point cancellation control**: $\Delta \geq 2\,\mathrm{dx}$
  ⇒ stencil never samples within a single grid cell, avoiding
  catastrophic cancellation.

For typical regimes (`τ ∈ [10⁻⁴, 10⁻¹]`, `dx ∈ [10⁻⁴, 10⁻²]`), the
two regimes meet near `τ ≈ 4·dx²`. Below this point the floor `2·dx`
dominates (correction's $\tau^2$ pre-factor still keeps total error
$O(\tau^2)$). Above this point $\sqrt{\tau}$ dominates and the
correction is local-$O(\tau^3)$ as designed.

**Boundary handling (BoundaryPolicy total over the stencil)**. All
five sample arguments — `f.sample(x)`, `f.sample(x ± Δ)`,
`f.sample(x ± 2Δ)` — MUST be obtained via `f.sample()` (which
dispatches through the active `BoundaryPolicy`: Reflect /
ZeroExtend / Periodic / LinearExtrapolate). Engineer **MUST NOT**
access `f.values[i ± k]` directly — that would silently break
boundary handling for nodes within `2Δ` of the edge, producing
order-degraded results in a thin boundary layer. The
`BoundaryPolicy` totality (Grid1D invariants I1–I5, §3.5) covers
all four variants without new boundary-handling code.

**`tau == 0` short-circuit**. The entire correction is gated on
`tau > 0`: for `tau == 0`, `tau*tau = 0` and the bracketed term
multiplies by zero. Combined with γ-A's `tau == 0 ⇒ D_γ = id`
(s_half = 0, h₀ = H₀ = 0, all sample points collapse to `x`,
weights sum to 1), we have `D_ζ(0) = D_γ(0) = id` (gate **Z_τ⁰**).

**Implementation pseudocode (additive over §9.2.3.A γ-A baseline)**:

```rust
// === γ-A baseline (preserved from §9.2.3.A) ===
let s_half     = 0.5 * tau;
let dx_pre     = s_half * (self.a_prime)(x);
let x_pre      = x + dx_pre;
let a_at_pre   = (self.a)(x_pre);
validate_a_x(a_at_pre, x_pre)?;
let h0         = 2.0 * libm::sqrt(a_at_pre * tau);
let H0         = 2.0 * libm::sqrt(3.0 * a_at_pre * tau);
let center_pos = x_pre + s_half * (self.a_prime)(x_pre);
let near_p_raw = x_pre + h0;
let near_p_pos = near_p_raw + s_half * (self.a_prime)(near_p_raw);
let near_n_raw = x_pre - h0;
let near_n_pos = near_n_raw + s_half * (self.a_prime)(near_n_raw);
let far_p_raw  = x_pre + H0;
let far_p_pos  = far_p_raw  + s_half * (self.a_prime)(far_p_raw);
let far_n_raw  = x_pre - H0;
let far_n_pos  = far_n_raw  + s_half * (self.a_prime)(far_n_raw);
let center     = W0 * f.sample(center_pos)?;
let near       = W1 * (f.sample(near_p_pos)? + f.sample(near_n_pos)?);
let far        = W2 * (f.sample(far_p_pos)?  + f.sample(far_n_pos)?);
let baseline   = center + near + far;

// === ζ-A τ² correction (NEW) ===
let a_x   = (self.a)(x);
let ap_x  = (self.a_prime)(x);
let app_x = (self.a_double_prime)(x);
// Δ = max(2·dx, √τ): super-grid for cancellation control,
// sub-√τ for τ-residual control. See §9.2.3.B "Δ choice".
let dx_grid = self.grid.dx();
let delta   = libm::sqrt(tau).max(2.0 * dx_grid);
let f0      = f.sample(x)?;
let fph     = f.sample(x + delta)?;          // f(x + Δ)
let fmh     = f.sample(x - delta)?;          // f(x - Δ)
let fp2     = f.sample(x + 2.0 * delta)?;    // f(x + 2Δ)
let fm2     = f.sample(x - 2.0 * delta)?;    // f(x - 2Δ)
// Central FD, all O(Δ²) accurate:
let f1      = (fph - fmh) / (2.0 * delta);                                    // f'(x)
let f2      = (fph - 2.0 * f0 + fmh) / (delta * delta);                       // f''(x)
let f3      = (fp2 - 2.0 * fph + 2.0 * fmh - fm2) / (2.0 * delta * delta * delta); // f'''(x)
// Pointwise correction polynomial:
let correction = tau * tau * (
        a_x * ap_x * f3
      + (a_x * app_x / 2.0) * f2
      + (ap_x * app_x / 4.0) * f1
);

result.values[i] = baseline + correction;
```

Total: `apply_at_node` ≈ 50 lines (right at the cap; the body has a
clear two-stage shape: γ-A baseline THEN ζ correction). File budget:
`diffusion.rs` ≤ 250 lines (≤ 30 LOC for ζ correction over γ-A's ≤ 220).

**Performance budget (ζ-A vs γ-A)**:

| Operation                         | γ-A | ζ-A | Δ vs γ-A |
|-----------------------------------|-----|-----|----------|
| `a(·)` evaluations                 | 1   | 2 (at `x_pre` + at `x` for correction) | +1 fn call |
| `a_prime(·)` evaluations           | 5   | 6 (γ + at `x` for correction)           | +1 fn call |
| `a_double_prime(·)` evaluations    | 0   | 1 (at `x`)                              | +1 fn call |
| `libm::sqrt`                       | 2   | 3 (γ + `√τ` for `Δ`)                    | +1 sqrt    |
| `f.sample`                         | 5   | 5 + 4 (γ + ζ stencil at `x±Δ, x±2Δ`)    | +4 sample  |
| Arithmetic (correction polynomial) | 0   | ~10 mul/add                             | negligible |
| **Total per-node latency**         | ~155-165 ns | **~205-225 ns** | **+30-50%** |

The +4 `f.sample` calls dominate the overhead (`f.sample` is ≈10-15 ns
each on x86_64 with cubic Hermite). Justification for accepting the
overhead: ζ delivers a TRUE order-2 lift for variable `a`. At fixed
accuracy target (e.g., `‖err‖_∞ ≤ 1e-3`), order-2 needs `O(√n)` fewer
steps than order-1, which more than compensates the per-step cost
(a 50% per-step slowdown is recouped after ~4× fewer steps, typical
for order-2 vs order-1 at fixed accuracy).

For **constant `a` callers** (`a_prime ≡ |_| 0.0`,
`a_double_prime ≡ |_| 0.0`), the entire correction
`(0·a'·f''') + (½·0·a''·f'') + (¼·0·0·f') = 0` constant-folds away.
The optimizer SHOULD eliminate all four extra `f.sample` calls in the
correction, restoring ~155 ns/node performance. Engineer Stage 6 MUST
verify via `cargo bench --bench heat_1d` (target: ±2% vs v0.2.2 for
constant α=0.5; ±50% otherwise per ADR-0008 Amendment 1 budget).

**Forward-compatibility (revised)**:
- **v0.4.0 (option ε, TruncatedExp) — SHIPPED, see §9.2.3.C**: ships
  `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` as a SIBLING type next to
  `DiffusionChernoff`, reusing the `(a, a', a'', a_norm, grid)`
  5-arg constructor verbatim plus an optional builder
  `with_drift_conjugation(b)`. One TruncatedExp step is
  $M(\tau) = \exp(\tau \cdot A_{\text{self}}^{I}(\tau/2))$ evaluated
  as a degree-4 truncated operator power series via the discrete
  3-point divergence-form stencil at grid spacing dx — avoiding FD
  on `f`-derivatives entirely. Lifts variable-`a` global rate from
  the ζ-A FD-ceiling $O(\tau^1)$ to $O(\tau^2)$. ζ-A is RETAINED as
  the constant-time-per-node fall-back; both ship in v0.4.0 to allow
  regression A/B testing.
- **v0.5.0+ (resolvent quadrature)**: reuses `(a, a', a'')` verbatim.
- **v0.6.0+ (`a'''` input for local-$O(\tau^4)$)**: would add a fourth
  closure. Sympy expansion of $D_\zeta$ to $O(\tau^4)$ shows the
  τ³ residual involves `a'''` — kill it by an analogous explicit τ³
  correction. Mathematically straightforward; deferred behind
  cost-benefit analysis.

#### Strang-composition order preservation (cross-ref §9.4 / §9.7)

`StrangSplit<DiffusionChernoff, DriftReactionChernoff>` order analysis
under the v0.3.0 (γ-A inner-Strang) upgrade:

- **Constant `a, b, c`** (the v0.2.0 production oracle, §9.5 / §9.7).
  By the §9.2.3 reduction lemma (`a' ≡ 0` ⇒ `S(s) = id` ⇒
  `D = K = D_{v0.2.2}` exactly), $D_\gamma$ is bit-identical to the
  v0.2.2 formula, so §9.4's analysis (commutator $[A, B] = 0$,
  $\Phi(\tau) = D(\tau/2)^2 \cdot e^{\tau B}$, slope $= -2$) applies
  verbatim. G1, G2, G3-strang, G4-strang **unchanged**.
- **Variable `a` (only)**: $D_\zeta$ is **local $O(\tau^3)$ / global
  $O(\tau^2)$** for variable `a ∈ C^3(\mathbb R)` (§9.2.3.B above —
  TRUE order-2 lift via the explicit τ²-correction polynomial, sympy
  gate **Z_τ²** zero deficit). The Strang composition
  $\Phi(\tau) = D_\zeta(\tau/2) \circ R(\tau) \circ D_\zeta(\tau/2)$
  with R local-$O(\tau^3)$ (constant `b, c` ⇒ exact characteristic;
  variable `b, c` ⇒ Amendment 5 RK2) yields **local $O(\tau^3)$ /
  global $O(\tau^2)$** for variable `a, b, c`. The palindromic-Strang
  $\tau^3$ commutator cancellation now kicks in for the variable-`a`
  regime as well, because **both** factors are local-$O(\tau^3)$
  under ζ-A. **Order-2 goal originally targeted by the rejected
  α formula is at last delivered correctly** — via correct generator
  ($A_{\text{self}} = \partial(a\partial)$) AND correct order-2 lift.
- **Variable `b, c` only (constant `a`)**: $D_\zeta$ collapses to
  $D_{v0.2.2}$ (sympy gate Z_const-a; correction is identically zero).
  $R$ is local $O(\tau^3)$ for variable `b, c` (Amendment 5). Strang
  gives global $O(\tau^2)$ in this regime — **Amendment 5 improvement
  preserved**.
- **Variable `a, b, c`** (the most general v0.3.0+ regime): **global
  $O(\tau^2)$** for the full operator. The "global $O(\tau^2)$ for
  variable `a, b, c`" claim from the rejected Amendment 6 (formula α)
  is now delivered correctly by ζ-A, with the divergence-form
  generator decomposition $A_{\text{self}} = \partial(a\partial)$ and
  caller-composed $b_{\text{total}} = b - a'$. The 2D tensor-product
  extension $\Phi^{2D}$ inherits the same per-axis order-2 result.

**Net effect on production gates**: G1, G2, G3-strang, G4-strang use
constant `a = 0.5`, so they observe $D_\zeta$ via the constant-`a`
fast path (bit-equal to v0.2.2 by sympy gate Z_const-a). All four
production gates pass with slopes ≤ -1.95 unchanged. v0.3.0 is
regression-safe for the production oracle. NEW gate (post-Stage 6,
Liouville oracle): variable-`a` slope ≤ -1.95 via property
`diffusion_chernoff_variable_zeta_liouville_oracle` (200 cases).

##### 9.2.3.C TruncatedExp integrator (NORMATIVE for v0.4.0, sibling to ζ-A)

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.4.0. Adds `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` as a
**sibling type** next to `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A); ζ-A is retained as
constant-time-per-node fall-back. Lifts variable-`a` global rate from
the ζ-A FD-ceiling $O(\tau^1)$ to $O(\tau^2)$ by avoiding FD on
`f`-derivatives entirely.

**Setting** (carries over from §9.2.3.A/B). Self-adjoint
divergence-form generator

$$
A_{\text{self}}\, f \;:=\; \partial_x\bigl(a(x)\,\partial_x f\bigr)
                       \;=\; a(x)\,f''(x) \;+\; a'(x)\,f'(x), \qquad a \in C^3(\mathbb R),\ \inf a > 0.
$$

The residual drift $-a'\partial$ is absorbed into $R$ via caller-composed
$b_{\text{total}} = b - a'$ (unchanged from §9.1.1). The residual
$B = b_{\text{total}}\,\partial + c$ is exposed below as the optional
interaction-picture conjugation parameter.

###### Interaction-picture (IP) conjugation

For the Strang-composition operator
$L = A_{\text{self}} + B$, the Magnus expansion of $\exp(\tau L)$ in
the **interaction picture** (HLW §III.5; Blanes–Casas–Oteo–Ros 2009 §2.3)
factors out the $B$-flow and writes

$$
\exp(\tau L) \;=\; \exp(\tau B) \cdot \mathcal{T}\,\exp\!\left(\int_0^\tau A_{\text{self}}^{I}(s)\,\mathrm{d}s\right),
\qquad
A_{\text{self}}^{I}(s) \;:=\; \exp(-s\,B)\,A_{\text{self}}\,\exp(+s\,B),
$$

where $\mathcal{T}$ is time-ordering. The order-2 truncation of the
time-ordered exponential is the **exponential midpoint rule**
(Munthe-Kaas 1995; HLW Theorem III.5.1):

$$
\boxed{\;
M(\tau) \;:=\; \exp\!\bigl(\tau \cdot A_{\text{self}}^{I}(\tau/2)\bigr) \;=\; \exp(\tau\,L) \;+\; O(\tau^3)\quad\text{(local)}.
\;}
$$

For the Strang composition $\Phi(\tau) = M(\tau/2) \circ R(\tau) \circ M(\tau/2)$,
the IP conjugation in $A_{\text{self}}^{I}(\tau/2)$ is **subsumed by the
outer Strang sandwich** — the Strang factors $\exp(\pm \tau B/2)$ already
provide the $\exp(-s B)$ conjugation kernel at the leading order. Therefore
the production Strang-composition path uses

$$
M(\tau)\,f(x) \;\approx\; \exp(\tau \cdot A_{\text{self}})\,f(x_{\text{mid}}),
\qquad x_{\text{mid}} \;:=\; x \;-\; \frac{\tau}{2}\,b(x),
$$

with $b \equiv 0$ when no drift conjugation is requested
(`with_drift_conjugation` not called); the foot-point collapses to
$x_{\text{mid}} = x$. The optional builder method enables the IP
foot-point shift for **non-Strang** integrators (e.g. matched-asymptotic
schemes); StrangSplit callers leave it `None`.

###### Truncated power series at degree K = 4

The exponential $\exp(\tau \cdot A_{\text{self}})$ is evaluated as a
**truncated operator power series**:

$$
M(\tau)\,f(x) \;\approx\; \sum_{k=0}^{K} \frac{\tau^k}{k!}\,\bigl(A_{\text{self}}\bigr)^k\,f(x_{\text{mid}})
\qquad K \;=\; 4 \;=:\; \texttt{MAGNUS\_TRUNC\_ORDER}.
$$

Factorial weights are precomputed:
$\bigl[1.0,\ 1.0,\ \tfrac{1}{2},\ \tfrac{1}{6},\ \tfrac{1}{24}\bigr]$.

**Per-step truncation residue** (BCOR 2009 Theorem 3, K-truncated
exponential):

$$
\Bigl\|\,M(\tau)\,f \;-\; \sum_{k=0}^{4} \tfrac{\tau^k}{k!}\,A_{\text{self}}^k f\,\Bigr\|_\infty
\;\leq\; \frac{(\tau \cdot \|A_{\text{self}}\|)^{5}}{5!}\,\|f\|_\infty
\;=\; \frac{(\tau\,\|G\|)^5}{120}\,\|f\|_\infty
\;=\; O(\tau^5).
$$

###### Discrete 3-point divergence-form stencil

The continuous operator $A_{\text{self}}$ is replaced by its discrete
analogue $G$ — the 3-point divergence-form stencil at grid spacing
$\mathrm{dx}$:

$$
\boxed{\;
G\,f\bigl|_i \;:=\; \frac{a_{i+½}\,(f_{i+1} - f_i) \;-\; a_{i-½}\,(f_i - f_{i-1})}{\mathrm{dx}^2}
\;}
$$

with $a_{i\pm½} := a(x_i \pm \mathrm{dx}/2)$ — the diffusion coefficient
evaluated at **half-grid-nodes** (NO a-grid required, just the closure
`a: fn(f64) -> f64`). The stencil is symmetric, second-order accurate,
and divergence-form-conservative.

Iterated $k$-fold action: $G^k f$ is computed by applying $G$ $k$ times
in a row, with two working buffers swapped each iteration:

```text
g_curr ← f_mid                  // k = 0
accum  ← f_mid                  // initial Σ_{k=0..0}-term
for k in 1..=4:
    g_next ← G · g_curr         // k-fold stencil (3-point)
    accum  ← accum  +  (τ^k / k!) · g_next
    swap(g_curr, g_next)
return accum
```

Stencil samples are **GRID-RESIDENT** at every step — there is no
off-grid `f.sample()` call (unlike ζ-A's $f.\text{sample}(x \pm \Delta)$
calls in the τ²-correction polynomial). This is the architectural fix
for the ζ-A H1 ceiling (§9.2.3.B / ADR-0008 Amendment 2 §H1).

Boundary indices $i = 0$ and $i = n-1$ require $f_{-1}$ / $f_n$, which
do not exist on-grid; these are obtained via the standard
`BoundaryPolicy` dispatch (Reflect / ZeroExtend / Periodic /
LinearExtrapolate) at the point $x_0 - \mathrm{dx}$ / $x_{n-1} + \mathrm{dx}$
respectively — same totality contract as ζ-A (Grid1D invariants I1–I5,
§3.5).

###### Per-step error bound

$$
\|\,M(\tau)\,f \;-\; \exp(\tau A_{\text{self}})\,f\,\|_\infty
\;\leq\; \underbrace{C_{\mathrm{stencil}}\,\mathrm{dx}^2\,\tau\,\|f^{(4)}\|_\infty}_{\substack{\text{stencil truncation}\\ O(\mathrm{dx}^2)}}
\;+\; \underbrace{\frac{(\tau\,\|G\|)^5}{120}\,\|f\|_\infty}_{\substack{\text{K=4 power-series residue}\\ O(\tau^5)}}.
$$

The two terms are independent:
- **Stencil truncation** is $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ from the central
  3-point Laplacian, scaled by the diffusion timescale $\tau$;
- **Power-series residue** is $O(\tau^5)$ at K=4 (`TRUNC_ORDER`).

For production grids ($\mathrm{dx} \approx 10^{-2}$, $\tau \approx 10^{-3}$),
the dominant term is the $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ stencil error;
$(\tau \|G\|)^5/120 \approx 10^{-15}$ is negligible.

###### CFL stability

The truncated power series at $K=4$ converges in operator norm iff
$\tau\,\|G\| < 2$ (BCOR 2009 §3.1: K=4 convergence bound for
factorial-weighted partial sums). With

$$
\|G\| \;\leq\; \frac{4\,\|a\|_\infty}{\mathrm{dx}^2}
\qquad (\text{Strikwerda, *Finite Difference Schemes*, §6.4: 3-point Laplacian eigenvalue bound}),
$$

the necessary condition becomes

$$
\boxed{\;
\tau \;<\; \frac{\mathrm{dx}^2}{2\,\|a\|_\infty}\quad (=:\ \tau_{\mathrm{CFL}}^{(K=4)})
\;}
$$

Violation triggers `SemiflowError::CflViolated { tau, dx_squared,
a_norm_bound }` (errors.yaml v0.4.0). The error variant is returned
**before any allocation** (suckless errors-as-values, guardrail #1).
Caller-side adaptive step-size pattern: retry with
$\tau_{\mathrm{safe}} := 0.45\cdot\mathrm{dx}^2 / \|a\|_\infty$ (90 %
CFL margin).

###### Global rate proof sketch (variable a)

For $a \in C^3(\mathbb R)$ strictly elliptic, iterating $M$ over
$n = T/\tau$ steps gives global error

$$
\|\,(M(\tau))^n\,f \;-\; \exp(T\,A_{\text{self}})\,f\,\|_\infty
\;\leq\; n \cdot \bigl(O(\mathrm{dx}^2 \tau) + O(\tau^5)\bigr)
\;=\; O(\mathrm{dx}^2) \;+\; O(\tau^4).
$$

The dominant term is $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ from the per-step stencil
error multiplied by $n = T/\tau$. The $\tau$-residue
$O(\tau^4)$ is below the $O(\tau^2)$ Strang-composition limit; in
the Strang sandwich $\Phi(\tau) = M(\tau/2) \circ R(\tau) \circ M(\tau/2)$,
the palindromic structure preserves the order-2 commutator
cancellation (HLW §III.5 Theorem 4.1), giving

$$
\boxed{\;
\bigl\|\,(\Phi(\tau))^n\,f \;-\; \exp(T\,L)\,f\,\bigr\|_\infty
\;=\; O(\mathrm{dx}^2) \;+\; O(\tau^2)
\quad\text{(global, variable } a, b, c \in C^3).
\;}
$$

— the implementation rate matches the theoretical rate, BREAKING the
ζ-A H1 FD-ceiling. References: HLW (Hairer–Lubich–Wanner) §III.4 +
Theorem 4.1; BCOR 2009 (Blanes–Casas–Oteo–Ros) Theorem 3; Remizov 2025
Theorem 6 (item 3).

###### Constant-a reduction lemma

When $a' \equiv 0$ and $a'' \equiv 0$ (caller passed $|\_|\;0.0$ for
both), $a_{i+½} = a_{i-½} = a_0$ identically, and the 3-point
divergence-form stencil collapses to the standard heat stencil:

$$
G_{\text{const}}\,f\bigl|_i
\;=\; \frac{a_0\,(f_{i+1} - f_i) - a_0\,(f_i - f_{i-1})}{\mathrm{dx}^2}
\;=\; a_0\cdot\frac{f_{i+1} - 2 f_i + f_{i-1}}{\mathrm{dx}^2}.
$$

Iterating $G_{\text{const}}^k$ and accumulating with factorial weights
gives the truncated-Taylor approximation of $\exp(\tau\,a_0\,\partial_x^2)\,f$
at the grid points — algebraically equivalent to the v0.2.2 K-only
formula at degree $K=4$ to within a per-step truncation residue
$O(\tau^5)$. For production CFL margins ($\tau \cdot a_0 / \mathrm{dx}^2 \leq 0.45$)
this residue is bounded by $(0.45\cdot 4)^5 / 120 \approx 1.6 \times 10^{-2}$
in the worst case — but the **G1, G2, G3-strang, G4-strang** production
gates all use $\tau \cdot a_0 / \mathrm{dx}^2 \approx 10^{-3}$ in
practice, giving residue $\leq 10^{-15}$. Property
`magnus_diffusion_constant_fast_path_close` enforces sup-norm agreement
$\|M - D_{v0.2.2}\|_\infty \leq 10^{-10}$ over 1000 random
$(\tau, a_0)$ pairs — close, NOT bit-equal (the truncation residue is
by construction non-zero, unlike ζ-A's algebraic identity).

###### Outer-Strang preservation: [M, R] vs. [D_ζ, R] commutator

The Strang-composition $\Phi(\tau) = D(\tau/2) \circ R(\tau) \circ D(\tau/2)$
has order-3 local truncation residue proportional to the operator
commutator $[A_{\text{self}}, B]$ (HLW §IV.2). Since $A_{\text{self}}$
and $B$ are **continuous** operators (independent of the discretization
of either), the commutator structure is unchanged from ζ-A:

$$
[D_{\zeta}, R](\tau)\,f \;=\; [M, R](\tau)\,f \;+\; O(\tau^3 \cdot \text{discretization}),
$$

i.e. the outer-Strang $\tau^3$ palindromic-cancellation argument that
makes G3-strang pass at slope $\leq -1.95$ for ζ-A applies verbatim to
TruncatedExp. The G3-strang gate transfers unchanged when D switches from
$D_\zeta$ to $M$.

###### Forward compatibility within v0.4.0
