ζ-A (`DiffusionChernoff`) is **retained** as constant-time-per-node
fall-back — callers who need ~155 ns/node and accept the variable-`a`
$O(\tau^1)$ ceiling stay on ζ-A. Callers who need true variable-`a`
$O(\tau^2)$ switch to `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` by changing one type
name (constructor signature is identical 5-arg). Both ship in v0.4.0
to enable A/B regression testing.

A future v0.5+ release MAY deprecate ζ-A once TruncatedExp has production
mileage; the deprecation is non-breaking (sibling type → main path
flip). v0.6.0+ `a'''` input would extend TruncatedExp to local-$O(\tau^4)$
via an analogous third-derivative correction term — additive over the
v0.4.0 stencil shape, no API break.

###### Documented runtime error: `SemiflowError::CflViolated`

NEW variant in v0.4.0 (errors.yaml schema v0.4.0). Returned by
`TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff::apply` when

$$
\tau \cdot \|a\|_\infty \;\geq\; \frac{\mathrm{dx}^2}{2}\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad 2\,\tau\,\|a\|_\infty \;\geq\; \mathrm{dx}^2.
$$

Payload `{ tau: f64, dx_squared: f64, a_norm_bound: f64 }` carries
the diagnostic triple for caller-side adaptive step-size control
(see CFL stability above). The check is the **first action** of
`apply` (after `tau` / `a_norm_bound` finiteness checks); no working
buffer is allocated when CFL is violated. ζ-A
(`DiffusionChernoff::apply`) does NOT emit `CflViolated` — its FD-based
scheme has unconditional $L^\infty$ stability via the positive-weight
K-factor; ζ-A's stability envelope is encoded as soft validity
constraints in `cev_european_call_sweep.yaml` rather than a runtime
error.

###### Retention rationale (sibling vs. replacement)

Why `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` ships **alongside** (not replacing)
`DiffusionChernoff`:

1. **Bit-equal regression for 10 constant-`a` call sites**. G1, G2,
   G3-strang, G4-strang and all v0.3.0 acceptance gates use constant
   `α = 0.5`; the ζ-A constant-`a` fast path is bit-equal to v0.2.2
   (sympy gate Z_const-a, NORMATIVE). TruncatedExp's constant-a reduction
   is *close* but not bit-equal (truncation residue $O(\tau^5)$).
   Retaining ζ-A preserves the algebraic regression guarantee for
   existing gates.
2. **Performance characteristics differ**. ζ-A is
   constant-time-per-node ($\sim$200 ns at K-fold loop K=0); TruncatedExp
   is K-fold ($\sim 4\times$ stencil cost ≈ 800 ns per node at K=4).
   For callers whose accuracy budget is satisfied by ζ-A's
   $O(\tau^1)$, the lower per-step cost is preferred.
3. **API stability invariant**. SemVer-minor v0.4.0 cannot remove
   `DiffusionChernoff` (would be a major break). Sibling-type
   addition is purely additive.
4. **Mathematical correctness vs. API priority**. User priority
   stated in the design plan (jazzy-sparking-taco): mathematical
   correctness > API stability. Sibling-type satisfies both — TruncatedExp
   delivers the correct rate; ζ-A retains the existing API contract.

A future v0.5+ release MAY deprecate `DiffusionChernoff` (not before;
deprecation requires production mileage on TruncatedExp across the
high-corner CEV regime that motivated it).

#### 9.2.4 v0.6.0 ζ⁴ extension — 4th-order spatial finite-difference on `f^{(k)}` (NORMATIVE for v0.6.0, sibling to ζ-A) ✅ ADOPTED

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.6.0. Adds `Diffusion4thChernoff` as a
**sibling type** next to `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A); ζ-A is retained as
constant-time-per-node fall-back (same retention rationale as ADR-0011
for TruncatedExp). Lifts the spatial finite-difference accuracy on the
$f^{(k)}$ derivatives inside the v0.3.0 ζ-A τ²-correction polynomial
from 2nd to 4th–6th order using the Fornberg (1988) 7-point central
stencils. The **γ-A baseline 5-point K-kernel is UNCHANGED** — its
weights $(7/12,\,3/16,\,1/48)$ already match the constant-`a` Fourier
symbol $e^{-a\tau\xi^2}$ to order $\xi^4$ (re-cite §9.2.1 derivation),
so the K-kernel is **already spatial 4th-order at fixed $\tau$**. The
only spatial-2nd-order locus in the v0.5.0 ζ-A path is the 5-point
central FD on $f', f'', f'''$ inside the τ²-correction; v0.6.0 lifts
ONLY that locus.

**Mechanism clarification (NORMATIVE, post-Phase-4 audit)**: The "K-kernel
4th-order spatial" claim above refers to the *Fourier-symbol* matching at
order ξ⁴ in the continuous limit (math.md §9.2.1). On a discrete grid with
smooth `f`, the leading uncancelled error from §9.2.1 is `(aτ)³·∂_x⁶f` —
purely temporal in the continuous sense.

The empirically observed 4th-order **spatial** slope in the 2D heat oracle
(G3⁴-2D measured slope = -3.99 over `N ∈ {400, 800, 1600}` at `n=2000`,
`T=0.5`, domain `[-15, 15]²`) arises from a different mechanism: the
cubic-Hermite interpolation kernel inside `f.sample(off-grid)` (ADR-0005)
has truncation error `O(dx⁴)` for `f ∈ C⁴`. Each K-kernel evaluation
samples `f` at shifted off-grid points `x ± h`, `x ± H`; these inherit
the cubic-Hermite floor. The Strang composition does not amplify it
(Theorem 7).

This means the 4th-order spatial benefit is **delivered jointly by**
(a) the continuous-Fourier ξ⁴-matched K-kernel weights and (b) the
cubic-Hermite interpolation. Either alone would not suffice.

For the τ²-correction term (which §9.2.4 lifts via 7-point central FD),
the spatial accuracy on f-derivatives is also bounded by cubic-Hermite at
the f.sample step plus FD truncation O(Δ⁴..Δ⁶). The choice
`Δ = max(3·dx, τ^{3/4})` ensures `Δ ≥ 3·dx` in production regime, so
the FD residue is the dominant source within the τ²-correction.

Empirical confirmation:
- Phase 1 1D constant-a: slope -3.93 over N ∈ {200..3200} at n=4000.
- Phase 1 1D variable-a Liouville (γ=0.05): slope -4.08 (D4th and D2
  agree because K-kernel + cubic-Hermite dominates at small γ).
- Phase 4 2D constant-a: slope -3.99 over N ∈ {400, 800, 1600} at
  n=2000. Ratios {7.27, 34.73}; the 34.73 ratio (>16=2⁴) confirms
  asymptotic dx⁴ regime is reached at N=1600.

**7-point Fornberg (1988) central FD weights**:

$$
f'(x) \;\approx\; \frac{1}{\Delta}\sum_{k=-3}^{3} c^{(1)}_k\,f(x + k\Delta),
\qquad c^{(1)} = \bigl(-\tfrac{1}{60},\,\tfrac{3}{20},\,-\tfrac{3}{4},\,0,\,\tfrac{3}{4},\,-\tfrac{3}{20},\,\tfrac{1}{60}\bigr),
\qquad \text{order } 6.
$$

$$
f''(x) \;\approx\; \frac{1}{\Delta^2}\sum_{k=-3}^{3} c^{(2)}_k\,f(x + k\Delta),
\qquad c^{(2)} = \bigl(\tfrac{1}{90},\,-\tfrac{3}{20},\,\tfrac{3}{2},\,-\tfrac{49}{18},\,\tfrac{3}{2},\,-\tfrac{3}{20},\,\tfrac{1}{90}\bigr),
\qquad \text{order } 6.
$$

$$
f'''(x) \;\approx\; \frac{1}{\Delta^3}\sum_{k=-3}^{3} c^{(3)}_k\,f(x + k\Delta),
\qquad c^{(3)} = \bigl(\tfrac{1}{8},\,-1,\,\tfrac{13}{8},\,0,\,-\tfrac{13}{8},\,1,\,-\tfrac{1}{8}\bigr),
\qquad \text{order } 4.
$$

The truncation residues are $f'_{\mathrm{FD}} - f' = O(\Delta^6)$,
$f''_{\mathrm{FD}} - f'' = O(\Delta^6)$, $f'''_{\mathrm{FD}} - f''' =
O(\Delta^4)$ (sympy gate **Z⁴_spatial-order** in
`verify_v0_6_0_zeta4.py` — leading coefficients
$f^{(7)}/140,\; f^{(8)}/560,\; -7\,f^{(7)}/120$ respectively).

**Stencil step `Δ` choice** (NORMATIVE):

$$
\boxed{\;
\Delta \;:=\; \max\bigl(3\,\mathrm{dx},\; \tau^{3/4}\bigr).
\;}
$$

Two competing concerns govern the `Δ`-budget:

- **Spatial truncation budget**: the τ²-correction's contribution to
  local error from FD residue is bounded by
  $\tau^2 \cdot O(\Delta^4)$ (the slowest of the three Fornberg
  orders, namely $f'''$). To keep this within the local-$O(\tau^5)$
  ζ⁴ budget we require $\tau^2 \cdot \Delta^4 \le \tau^5$, i.e.
  $\Delta \le \tau^{3/4}$.
- **Floating-point cancellation budget**: with stencil step
  $\Delta \ll \mathrm{dx}$, the 7-point central FD on cubic-Hermite
  $f.\mathrm{sample}(x \pm k\Delta)$ at sub-grid distances suffers
  catastrophic cancellation in $(f(x+\Delta) - f(x-\Delta))/(2\Delta)$
  — the Hermite splines coincide to many digits at sub-grid range,
  and the difference loses precision proportional to
  $\varepsilon_{\mathrm{mach}}/\Delta$. To stay safely above the
  cubic-Hermite reconstruction noise floor we require the stencil to
  span at least 6 grid cells, i.e. $3\Delta \ge 3\,\mathrm{dx}$,
  giving $\Delta \ge \mathrm{dx}$ at minimum and $\Delta \ge 3\,\mathrm{dx}$
  for the $\pm 3\Delta$ outermost arms.

The `max(3·dx, τ^{3/4})` floor combines both: the lower bound `3·dx`
dominates in the production regime ($\mathrm{dx} \approx 10^{-2}$,
$\tau \approx 10^{-3} \Rightarrow \tau^{3/4} \approx 5.6 \times 10^{-3}
\le 3\,\mathrm{dx}$), and the `τ^{3/4}` upper bound activates only at
very fine `dx` or very coarse `τ` (an asymptotic regime not exercised
by v0.6.0 acceptance gates).

**Definition of $D_{\zeta^4}(\tau)$** (NORMATIVE):

$$
\boxed{\;
\begin{aligned}
D_{\zeta^4}(\tau) f(x) \;&:=\; D_\gamma(\tau) f(x) \;+\; \tau^2 \cdot \mathcal{C}^4[a, a', a''](x; f, \Delta),\\[8pt]
\mathcal{C}^4[a, a', a''](x; f, \Delta) \;&:=\;
   a(x)\,a'(x)\,f'''_{\mathrm{FD}^4}(x; \Delta)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{2}\,a(x)\,a''(x)\,f''_{\mathrm{FD}^6}(x; \Delta)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{4}\,a'(x)\,a''(x)\,f'_{\mathrm{FD}^6}(x; \Delta),
\end{aligned}
\;}
$$

with $D_\gamma(\tau) = S(\tau/2) \circ K(\tau;a) \circ S(\tau/2)$
**bit-equal to the v0.3.0 / v0.5.0 γ-A baseline** (the K-kernel weights,
the S-shift, and the $h_0/H_0$ formulas are unchanged) and the FD
operators using the 7-point Fornberg coefficients above.

**Sympy-verified gates** (`verify_v0_6_0_zeta4.py`, exit 0 on success):

- **Z⁴_τ⁰** (identity): $D_{\zeta^4}(0)\,f|_0 = f_0$ ✓ (deficit $0$ exact).
- **Z⁴_τ¹** (Chernoff consistency): $[\tau^1] D_{\zeta^4}(\tau)f|_0 =
  a_0 f_2 + a_1 f_1 = A_{\mathrm{self}} f|_0$ ✓ — algebraically zero
  deficit.
- **Z⁴_τ²** (TRUE order-2 lift, NORMATIVE): the τ²-deficit
  $[\tau^2]\bigl(D_{\zeta^4}(\tau)f - e^{\tau A_{\mathrm{self}}}f\bigr)|_0$
  is **identically zero** in the polynomial ring of
  $(f_0,\ldots,f_6,\,a_0,\ldots,a_3)$ when the FD operators are replaced
  by their analytic limits — this gate is INHERITED from the v0.3.0 ζ-A
  proof. The implementation gate is then determined by the FD-residue
  scaling Z⁴_spatial-order: $\tau^2 \cdot O(\Delta^4) \le O(\tau^5)$ for
  $\Delta = \tau^{3/4}$, and $\tau^2 \cdot O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ in the
  $\Delta = 3\,\mathrm{dx}$ floor regime.
- **Z⁴_const-a** (constant-`a` regression): when $a' \equiv 0 \wedge
  a'' \equiv 0$, the correction polynomial vanishes identically AND
  $S(s) = \mathrm{id}$, so $D_{\zeta^4} = K(\tau;a_0) \equiv$ v0.5.0
  bit-equal. ✓ NORMATIVE.
- **Z⁴_spatial-order**: 7-point FD truncation residues
  $f' = O(\Delta^6)$, $f'' = O(\Delta^6)$, $f''' = O(\Delta^4)$ ✓
  NORMATIVE.

**Order claim** (math.md §9.2.4):

| Regime | Local order (per step) | Global Strang order | Generator |
|--------|------------------------|---------------------|-----------|
| Constant `a`             | $O(\tau^3)$ exact (γ-A K-only; correction ≡ 0) | $O(\tau^2)$ via Strang | $A$ ✓ (= $A_{\mathrm{self}}$) |
| Variable `a \in C^5(\mathbb R)` | $O(\tau^5)$ at $\Delta = \tau^{3/4}$; $O(\tau^2 \cdot \mathrm{dx}^4)$ at $\Delta = 3\,\mathrm{dx}$ | $O(\tau^2)$ in $\tau$ ⊕ $O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ in `dx` | $A_{\mathrm{self}}$ ✓ |
| Variable `a, b, c` (full) | limited by R: $O(\tau^2)$ | $O(\tau^2) \oplus O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ | $L = A_{\mathrm{self}} + B_{\mathrm{compensated}}$ ✓ |

**Crucial difference vs. v0.5.0 ζ-A**: variable-`a` global rate stays
at $O(\tau^2)$ from Strang composition, BUT the spatial leading constant
is $O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ instead of $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ — at production
$\mathrm{dx} \approx 10^{-2}$ this is a $10^{-4}$ vs $10^{-8}$ floor
shift, lifting the achievable accuracy by ~four decimal digits before
the spatial floor saturates the τ-convergence (math.md §9.7 / §9.2.7
spatial-error budget — the same model that calibrated v0.3.0's required
$N$ for G3-strang now applies with `dx⁴` in place of `dx²`).

**Caller invariants** (NEW vs. v0.5.0 ζ-A):

- $a \in C^5(\mathbb R)$ strictly elliptic with bounded derivatives
  through order 6 (the 7-point Fornberg stencil for $f$ amplifies
  $f^{(7)}$ at coefficient $1/140$ — bounded $f^{(7)}$ keeps the
  residue tight). v0.5.0 ζ-A required only $C^3$.
- The 7-point FD stencil samples $f$ at $x \pm k\Delta$ for $k \in
  \{1, 2, 3\}$. Boundary nodes (interior less than $3\Delta$ from the
  edge) route through `BoundaryPolicy` via `f.sample()` — same totality
  contract as v0.5.0 ζ-A's 5-point stencil; no new boundary code is
  required.
- Production callers SHOULD pad the working domain to ≥ 5σ from the
  initial-data support (Risk R5 in the design plan) — within
  $3\Delta = 9\,\mathrm{dx}$ of the edge the boundary-policy branch is
  exercised at every step, which (for `Reflect`) does not affect
  asymptotic order but does add a per-step constant-factor cost.

**Forward compatibility**:

- v0.7+ MAY add an even-higher-order ζ⁶ variant using 9-point FD
  ($O(\Delta^8)/O(\Delta^8)/O(\Delta^6)$) — additive over the v0.6.0
  shape, no API break (constructor is identical 5-arg with same
  closures `(a, a', a'', a_norm, grid)`).
- v0.6.0 reuses the v0.5.0 ζ-A 5-arg constructor verbatim — callers
  switch from ζ-A to ζ⁴ by changing one type name
  (`DiffusionChernoff` → `Diffusion4thChernoff`).

#### 9.2.5 v0.6.0 TruncatedExp⁴ — 4th-order divergence-form spatial stencil (NORMATIVE for v0.6.0, sibling to TruncatedExp K=4) ✅ ADOPTED

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.6.0. Adds `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff` as
a **sibling type** next to `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` (v0.4.0); the
v0.4.0 type is retained as the constant-time-per-node fall-back. The
K=4 truncated power series formula and the IP foot-point construction
are **unchanged**; the only modification is the **discrete divergence-
form stencil $G \to G^4$** lifting from 3-point to 5-point.

**5-point divergence-form stencil $G^4$** (Architect-derived, sympy-
verified):

$$
\boxed{\;
G^4 f\bigl|_i \;:=\; \frac{1}{\mathrm{dx}^2}\Bigl[
   -\,\tfrac{1}{12}\,a_{i+\tfrac{3}{2}}(f_{i+2} - f_{i+1})
   \;+\;\tfrac{5}{4}\,a_{i+\tfrac{1}{2}}(f_{i+1} - f_i)
   \;-\;\tfrac{5}{4}\,a_{i-\tfrac{1}{2}}(f_i - f_{i-1})
   \;+\;\tfrac{1}{12}\,a_{i-\tfrac{3}{2}}(f_{i-1} - f_{i-2})
\Bigr],
\;}
$$

with $a_{i\pm k/2} := (\mathrm{self.a})(x_i \pm k\,\mathrm{dx}/2)$ for
$k \in \{1, 3\}$ — the closure is now evaluated at FOUR half-grid
positions per node (vs. two for the v0.4.0 3-point stencil; +2 closure
calls per node).

**Architect correction (sympy-derived, NORMATIVE)**: an early v0.6.0
plan draft proposed flux coefficients $(7/6, -7/6)$ at the
$\pm 1/2$ shifts, but sympy gate M⁴_const-a-fast in
`verify_v0_6_0_magnus4.py` showed that those would collapse to the
non-standard 5-point Laplacian $[-1/12, 5/4, -7/3, 5/4, -1/12]\,a_0/\mathrm{dx}^2$.
The corrected coefficients $(5/4, -5/4)$ enforce the **standard 4th-
order central Laplacian** collapse for constant $a$:

$$
G^4 f\bigl|_i \;\stackrel{a \equiv a_0}{=}\;
\frac{a_0}{\mathrm{dx}^2}\,\bigl[\,-\tfrac{1}{12} f_{i-2}
    \;+\;\tfrac{4}{3} f_{i-1}
    \;-\;\tfrac{5}{2} f_i
    \;+\;\tfrac{4}{3} f_{i+1}
    \;-\;\tfrac{1}{12} f_{i+2}\,\bigr],
$$

— sympy gate M⁴_const-a-fast in `verify_v0_6_0_magnus4.py` (residual
identically zero in the polynomial ring of $f_0, \ldots, f_8$).

**Honest variable-`a` spatial-order claim** (NORMATIVE, **differs from
the constant-`a` claim**):

| Regime | $G^4 f - A_{\mathrm{self}} f|_0$ leading order | Leading coefficient |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| Constant `a` ($a' \equiv \cdots \equiv 0$) | $O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ | $-a_0\,f^{(6)}/90$ |
| Variable `a \in C^5(\mathbb R)` | $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ | $-a'\,f'''/12 - a''\,f''/8 - a'''\,f'/24$ |

Sympy gate M⁴_spatial-order in `verify_v0_6_0_magnus4.py` (NORMATIVE)
confirms both rows. The **variable-`a` leading $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$
residue is impossible to eliminate** with any 5-point divergence-form
stencil sampling $a$ only at half-grid points (Strikwerda, *Finite
Difference Schemes*, §6.4 + Mickens 1994 §3.2 — central symmetric flux
schemes hit a parity wall at variable-coefficient 4th-order). The
v0.6.0 honest claim is therefore: **4th-order spatial AT CONSTANT $a$
ONLY**; for variable $a$ the leading dx²-coefficient is strictly
smaller than the v0.4.0 3-point stencil (Mickens-improvement: ~3×
constant reduction), but the asymptotic order is the same. **A genuine
variable-`a` 4th-order divergence-form stencil** would require sampling
$a$ at both grid AND half-grid points (11+ closure evaluations per
node) and is deferred to v0.7+ behind a separate ADR.

**Observable benefit despite the variable-`a` honesty**: the v0.6.0
release gate G3⁴-2D (math.md §10.5(a) heat oracle, eq. 10.7) is at
**constant $a = 1/2$ per axis** — exactly the regime where the 4th-
order spatial collapse is active. The headline 2D slope target
$\le -3.80$ is reachable because the 2D heat oracle has constant
coefficients per axis; CEV diffusion (variable $a$) gets a tighter
constant in the same $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ envelope.

**New CFL stability bound** (NORMATIVE, errors.yaml v0.4.0 reused
verbatim):

$$
\|G^4\| \;\le\; \frac{16\,\|a\|_\infty}{3\,\mathrm{dx}^2}
\qquad
\text{(eigenvalue bound, Fourier symbol at $k\,\mathrm{dx} = \pi$).}
$$

The Fourier symbol of the constant-`$a$` stencil
$[-\tfrac{1}{12},\tfrac{4}{3},-\tfrac{5}{2},\tfrac{4}{3},-\tfrac{1}{12}]\,a_0/\mathrm{dx}^2$
is

$$
\hat G^4(\xi) \;=\; \frac{a_0}{\mathrm{dx}^2}\bigl(-\tfrac{1}{6}\cos(2\xi\,\mathrm{dx}) + \tfrac{8}{3}\cos(\xi\,\mathrm{dx}) - \tfrac{5}{2}\bigr),
$$

attaining its extremum at $\xi\,\mathrm{dx} = \pi$ where
$\cos(\pi) = -1, \cos(2\pi) = 1$:
$\hat G^4(\pi/\mathrm{dx}) = \tfrac{a_0}{\mathrm{dx}^2}(-\tfrac{1}{6} - \tfrac{8}{3} - \tfrac{5}{2}) = -\tfrac{a_0}{\mathrm{dx}^2} \cdot \tfrac{32}{6} = -\tfrac{16\,a_0}{3\,\mathrm{dx}^2}$.

K=4 power-series convergence requires $\tau\,\|G^4\| < 2$ (BCOR 2009
§3.1, unchanged), giving the necessary CFL

$$
\boxed{\;
\tau \;<\; \frac{3\,\mathrm{dx}^2}{8\,\|a\|_\infty} \quad (=:\ \tau_{\mathrm{CFL}}^{(K=4,4)}).
\;}
$$

**This is 25% tighter than the v0.4.0 CFL** $\tau < \mathrm{dx}^2/(2\|a\|_\infty)$
because $\|G^4\| / \|G\| = \tfrac{16/3}{4} = \tfrac{4}{3}$ — the wider
stencil has a strictly larger eigenvalue at the Nyquist mode.
Implementation MUST encode the new bound via the constants

```rust
pub const CFL_NUMER: u32 = 3;  // renamed from MAGNUS4_CFL_NUMER in v0.7.0
pub const CFL_DENOM: u32 = 8;  // renamed from MAGNUS4_CFL_DENOM in v0.7.0
```

distinct from the v0.4.0 `TRUNC_CFL_NUMER = 1, TRUNC_CFL_DENOM = 2`.
The error variant `SemiflowError::CflViolated { tau, dx_squared,
a_norm_bound }` is **reused verbatim from v0.4.0** — no new variant is
added (the `dx_squared` and `a_norm_bound` payload diagnoses both v0.4.0
and v0.6.0 CFL violations; the caller decides the safe-retry formula
based on which type returned the error).

**Per-step error bound** (NORMATIVE):

$$
\|\,M^4(\tau)\,f \;-\; \exp(\tau A_{\mathrm{self}})\,f\,\|_\infty
\;\leq\; \underbrace{C^4_{\mathrm{stencil},a}\,\mathrm{dx}^4\,\tau\,\|f^{(6)}\|_\infty}_{\substack{\text{constant-}a \text{ stencil truncation}\\ O(\mathrm{dx}^4)}}
\;+\; \underbrace{C^4_{\mathrm{stencil},\partial a}\,\mathrm{dx}^2\,\tau\,\|a^{(k)}\,f^{(j)}\|_\infty}_{\substack{\text{variable-}a \text{ residue}\\ O(\mathrm{dx}^2)}}
\;+\; \underbrace{\frac{(\tau\,\|G^4\|)^5}{120}\,\|f\|_\infty}_{\substack{\text{K=4 power-series residue}\\ O(\tau^5)}}.
$$

**Outer-Strang preservation** (cross-ref §9.2.3.C "Outer-Strang
preservation" — CARRIES OVER VERBATIM): the commutator $[A_{\mathrm{self}},
B]$ in the order-3 Strang truncation residue depends only on the
*continuous* $A_{\mathrm{self}}$ and $B$; the discretization $G^4$
does not enter the commutator structure. Therefore the outer-Strang
$\tau^3$ palindromic-cancellation argument that makes G3-strang pass
at slope $\le -1.95$ for v0.4.0 TruncatedExp applies verbatim to TruncatedExp⁴,
and the global Strang composition $\Phi^4(\tau) = M^4(\tau/2) \circ
R(\tau) \circ M^4(\tau/2)$ retains $O(\tau^2) \oplus O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$
in the constant-`a` regime (G3⁴-2D oracle) and $O(\tau^2) \oplus
O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ for variable-`a` (CEV-style diffusion).

**Constant-`a` reduction (close, NOT bit-equal)**: when $a' \equiv 0
\wedge a'' \equiv 0$, $G^4_{\mathrm{const}} = a_0\,[-\tfrac{1}{12},
\tfrac{4}{3}, -\tfrac{5}{2}, \tfrac{4}{3}, -\tfrac{1}{12}]/\mathrm{dx}^2$
is the standard 4th-order central Laplacian; the K=4 truncated power
series $\sum (\tau a_0 / \mathrm{dx}^2)^k / k! \cdot \partial^{2k}_4 f$
agrees with the closed-form heat semigroup $e^{\tau a_0 \partial_x^2}
f$ to local-$O(\tau^5)$. Property
`magnus4_constant_fast_path_close` enforces sup-norm agreement
$\|M^4 - M^{(\mathrm{v0.4.0})}\|_\infty \le 10^{-10}$ over 1000 random
$(\tau, a_0)$ pairs in the constant-$a$ regime — close, not bit-equal:
the 5-point stencil at constant $a$ converges to the same continuous
limit as the v0.4.0 3-point stencil but with different $O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$
floor coefficients.

**Caller invariants** (NEW vs. v0.4.0 TruncatedExp):

- $a \in C^5(\mathbb R)$ strictly elliptic with bounded derivatives
  through order 6 (the constant-$a$ residue carries $f^{(6)}$;
  variable-$a$ residue carries $a^{(3)} \cdot f'$). v0.4.0 required only
  $C^3$.
- Per-node closure cost: 4 `(self.a)` evaluations at half-grid points
  $x_i \pm \mathrm{dx}/2, x_i \pm 3\,\mathrm{dx}/2$ (vs. 2 for v0.4.0).
  Total per-step cost is `n * 4 * (a-eval) + n * (K+1) * stencil-flop`
  ≈ $4\times$ closure-call overhead vs. v0.4.0.

**Forward compatibility**:

- v0.7+ MAY add a 7-point compact divergence-form stencil sampling $a$
  at full-grid AND half-grid points (11 closure evaluations per node)
  to break the variable-$a$ $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ wall — additive over
  v0.6.0 shape, no API break.
- The `TRUNC_ORDER` constant is unchanged at $K = 4$.
- Constructor signature is identical 5-arg
  `(a, a_prime, a_double_prime, a_norm_bound, grid)` — drop-in
  replacement for `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` by changing one type name.

#### 9.2.6 v0.7.0 ζ⁶ extension — 6th-order spatial (NORMATIVE for v0.7.0, sibling to ζ⁴) ✅ ADOPTED

> **Status: NORMATIVE for v0.7.0 release.** Additive sibling to
> `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A, v0.3.0) and `Diffusion4thChernoff` (ζ⁴, v0.6.0).
> All v0.5.0/v0.6.0 callers remain bit-equal — sibling addition only.
> Cross-ref: ADR-0015. Sympy gates in
> `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_7_0_kkernel.py`,
> `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`, `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py` — all exit 0.

`Diffusion6thChernoff` implements **genuine 6th-order spatial accuracy** for
$A_{\mathrm{self}} = \partial_x(a(x)\,\partial_x)$ via three concurrent lifts
over the v0.6.0 ζ⁴ path (ADR-0015, Plan-1 FULL lift):

**(a)** 7-point K-kernel (`γ⁶-A` baseline) replacing the v0.5.0 5-point K;
**(b)** 9-point Fornberg central FD replacing the v0.6.0 7-point Fornberg;
**(c)** `InterpKind::QuinticHermite` replacing Catmull-Rom `CubicHermite`.

**Mechanism note (NORMATIVE)**: `slope = min(FD-order, K-kernel-order,
interpolant-order)`. With all three lifted to O(dx⁶), the minimum is 6.
Removing any one component drops the slope back to 4 (the ζ⁴ regime).

The ζ⁶ formula is:

$$D_{\zeta^6}(\tau)\,f(x) = D_{\gamma^6}(\tau)\,f(x)
  + \tau^2\!\left[\,a\,a'\,f''' + \tfrac12 a\,a''\,f'' + \tfrac14 a'\,a''\,f'\,\right]$$

where $f', f'', f'''$ are computed by the 9-point Fornberg FD stencil
at stencil step $\Delta$.  This is the **same τ²-correction polynomial
structure** as §9.2.3.B (ζ-A) and §9.2.4 (ζ⁴); only the FD order and
K-kernel arm count are lifted.

---

**7-point K-kernel (γ⁶-A baseline)**

$$\boxed{K_7\,f\big|_x = w_0\,f(x)
  + w_1\bigl[f(x+h)+f(x-h)\bigr]
  + w_2\bigl[f(x+H)+f(x-H)\bigr]
  + w_3\bigl[f(x+J)+f(x-J)\bigr]}$$

with $h = 2\sqrt{a\tau}$, $H = 2\sqrt{3a\tau}$, $J = 2\sqrt{5a\tau}$
(scale multiplier $P = 5$, chosen for tightest positive-weight solution).

Weights (rational, NORMATIVE — `verify_v0_7_0_kkernel.py`):

| Symbol | Value    | Float             |
|--------|----------|-------------------|
| $w_0$  | 67/120   | 0.558 333...      |
| $w_1$  | 27/128   | 0.210 937 5       |
| $w_2$  | 1/192    | 0.005 208...      |
| $w_3$  | 3/640    | 0.004 687 5       |

Leading uncancelled residue: $+s^4/280 \cdot \xi^8$ (gate `K7_leading_residue`).
All weights positive → sub-Markov / probability interpretation preserved.

---

**9-point Fornberg (1988) central FD coefficients** (offsets $k = -4\ldots+4$):

$f'$ stencil (O(Δ⁸)):

$$\bigl[+\tfrac{1}{280},\,-\tfrac{4}{105},\,+\tfrac{1}{5},\,-\tfrac{4}{5},\,0,\,+\tfrac{4}{5},\,-\tfrac{1}{5},\,+\tfrac{4}{105},\,-\tfrac{1}{280}\bigr]\,/\,\Delta$$

$f''$ stencil (O(Δ⁸)):

$$\bigl[-\tfrac{1}{560},\,+\tfrac{8}{315},\,-\tfrac{1}{5},\,+\tfrac{8}{5},\,-\tfrac{205}{72},\,+\tfrac{8}{5},\,-\tfrac{1}{5},\,+\tfrac{8}{315},\,-\tfrac{1}{560}\bigr]\,/\,\Delta^2$$

$f'''$ stencil (O(Δ⁶)):

$$\bigl[-\tfrac{7}{240},\,+\tfrac{3}{10},\,-\tfrac{169}{120},\,+\tfrac{61}{30},\,0,\,-\tfrac{61}{30},\,+\tfrac{169}{120},\,-\tfrac{3}{10},\,+\tfrac{7}{240}\bigr]\,/\,\Delta^3$$

---

**Quintic-Hermite interpolant** (`InterpKind::QuinticHermite`)

Degree-5 polynomial on each cell $[x_i, x_{i+1}]$ using scaled nodal data
$(F_0, F_{0p}, F_{0pp}, F_1, F_{1p}, F_{1pp})$ where $F_{0p} = \mathrm{dx}\,f'(x_i)$
and $F_{0pp} = \mathrm{dx}^2\,f''(x_i)$ (ghost data computed via central FD).
Weight polynomials (sympy-derived, NORMATIVE, `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py`):

| Poly  | Expression                                      |
|-------|-------------------------------------------------|
| $a_0$ | $-6s^5 + 15s^4 - 10s^3 + 1$                    |
| $a_1$ | $-3s^5 + 8s^4 - 6s^3 + s$                      |
| $a_2$ | $-s^5/2 + 3s^4/2 - 3s^3/2 + s^2/2$             |
| $b_0$ | $6s^5 - 15s^4 + 10s^3$                          |
| $b_1$ | $-3s^5 + 7s^4 - 4s^3$                           |
| $b_2$ | $s^5/2 - s^4 + s^3/2$                           |

Leading residue: $f^{(6)}/720 \cdot s^3(1-s)^3 \cdot \mathrm{dx}^6$, bounded
$\le \mathrm{dx}^6/46080$ at $s = 1/2$.

---

**Stencil step**

$$\boxed{\Delta = \max(4\,\mathrm{dx},\; \tau^{1/2})}$$

Derivation: spatial truncation budget from the $f'''$ FD is
$\tau^2 \cdot O(\Delta^6)$; setting $\Delta = \tau^{1/2}$ gives
$\tau^2 \cdot \tau^3 = O(\tau^5)$, inside the local-$O(\tau^5)$ ζ⁶ budget.
Floor $4\,\mathrm{dx}$ keeps the outermost arm ($\pm 4\Delta$) at
$\ge 16$ grid cells from center (FP cancellation budget for quintic-Hermite
ghost data).

---

**ζ⁶ definition (NORMATIVE)**

$$\boxed{D_{\zeta^6}(\tau) = D_{\gamma^6}(\tau)
  + \tau^2\!\left[\,a\,a'\,f'''_{{\rm FD9}} + \tfrac12 a\,a''\,f''_{{\rm FD9}}
    + \tfrac14 a'\,a''\,f'_{{\rm FD9}}\,\right]}$$

where $D_{\gamma^6}(\tau) = S(\tau/2) \circ K_7(\tau;a) \circ S(\tau/2)$
is the γ⁶-A baseline (7-point K-kernel, Strang-half-transports).

---

**Sympy-verified gates** (all exit 0):

| Gate                 | Content                                           | Script                         |
|----------------------|---------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------|
| `K7_sum_to_1`        | $w_0 + 2(w_1+w_2+w_3) = 1$ (sub-Markov)          | `verify_v0_7_0_kkernel.py`     |
| `K7_xi6_match`       | Fourier symbol matches $e^{-s\xi^2}$ through ξ⁶  | `verify_v0_7_0_kkernel.py`     |
| `K7_leading_residue` | Leading residue $+s^4/280 \cdot \xi^8$            | `verify_v0_7_0_kkernel.py`     |
| `Z6_tau0`            | $D_{\zeta^6}(0)\,f = f$ (identity)                | `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`       |
| `Z6_tau1`            | $[\tau^1]$: $D_{\zeta^6}\,f = A_{\rm self}\,f$   | `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`       |
| `Z6_tau2`            | $[\tau^2]$ deficit = 0 (TRUE order-2 lift)        | `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`       |
| `Z6_const_a`         | $a'\equiv a''\equiv 0 \Rightarrow$ correction = 0 | `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`       |
| `Z6_spatial_order`   | 9-pt FD truncation O(Δ⁸)/O(Δ⁸)/O(Δ⁶)            | `verify_v0_7_0_zeta6.py`       |
| `QHerm5_partition`   | $a_0 + b_0 \equiv 1$ (partition of unity)         | `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py` |
| `QHerm5_endpoints`   | 6 boundary conditions satisfied                   | `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py` |
| `QHerm5_consistency` | Degree-5 polynomial reproduction (residue = 0)   | `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py` |
| `QHerm5_order`       | Leading residue O(dx⁶) with predicted coefficient| `verify_v0_7_0_quintic_hermite.py` |

---

**Order claim table**

| Component            | Spatial order | Τ-axis order |
|----------------------|---------------|--------------|
| γ⁶-A (K7 baseline)  | 6             | 2            |
| ζ⁶ τ²-correction     | 6             | 2            |
| QuinticHermite interp| 6             | —            |
| **ζ⁶ combined**      | **6**         | **2**        |

**Slope gate G3⁶** (NORMATIVE for v0.7.0 release, math.md §10):

$$\text{slope}_{\mathrm{G3^6}} \le -5.85 \quad\text{(expected achieved}\approx -5.95 \pm 0.10\text{)}$$

**Test grid (NORMATIVE)**: 1D heat oracle on $N \in \{251, 503, 997, 1999, 3989\}$ at
$n = 4000$, $T = 0.5$, domain $[-15, 15]$, constant $a = 0.5$. Prime-based N is chosen
deliberately: dyadic doublings (200, 400, 800, …) trigger **K7-grid resonance** — the K7
kernel uses fixed shifts $h = 2\sqrt{a\tau}$ that resonate with $\mathrm{dx} = L/N$ at
dyadic N, producing non-monotone fractional offsets $s = \{h/\mathrm{dx}\}$ and distorting
the OLS slope from its asymptotic value. Prime N values break the resonance pattern by
avoiding common factors with $h$, recovering the genuine 6th-order convergence.
(Reference: bug-fixer diagnosis, v0.7.0 Block B retrospective.)

**`order()` returns 2** (τ-axis Chernoff order; see math.md §11.1.bis ratified
in v0.6.1 audit — spatial slope is a dx-axis property verified by G3⁶, NOT
advertised by `order()`).

---

**Caller invariants**

- $a(x) > 0$ everywhere (strict ellipticity).
- $a \in C^7(\mathbb R)$ with bounded derivatives through order 8
  (NEW vs. ζ⁴ which required C⁵).
- For constant $a$: pass `|_| 0.0_f64` for both derivatives; τ²-correction
  vanishes (gate `Z6_const_a`); K7 baseline is NOT bit-equal to v0.5.0
  (it uses the new 7-point kernel — 6th-order Fourier match vs. 4th-order
  for the 5-point v0.5.0 kernel).
- Grid must have `n >= 4` (existing `Grid1D::new` invariant).

---

**Mechanism recap (NORMATIVE)**

The 6th-order spatial accuracy is achieved JOINTLY by three concurrent lifts.
Any single-component lift saturates at slope 4 (ζ⁴ regime). The K7 + FD9 +
QuinticHermite combination is the unique minimal set that delivers genuine dx⁶.

**Forward compatibility**

- v0.7.0 reuses the v0.5.0 5-arg constructor verbatim.
- `InterpKind::QuinticHermite` defaults to OFF (`Grid1D::new` defaults to
  `CubicHermite`); opt in via `.with_interp(InterpKind::QuinticHermite)`.
- v0.8+ MAY add ζ⁸ (11-pt Fornberg + 9-pt K-kernel + septic-Hermite),
  additive over v0.7.0, no API break.

#### 9.2.6.bis v4.2 Path ε — QuinticHermite propagation to K5 + ζ-ladder (NORMATIVE for v4.2, ADR-0089)

> **Status: NORMATIVE for v4.2 release.** Architectural retrofit only — the
> `InterpKind::QuinticHermite` kernel and its `sample_quintic_1d` impl in
> `crates/semiflow-core/src/grid_quintic.rs` (208 LoC, sympy-verified via
> `QHerm5_partition` / `QHerm5_endpoints` / `QHerm5_consistency` / `QHerm5_order`)
> are unchanged from v0.7.0 (§9.2.6). Path ε only changes WHICH kernels opt in.

Path ε propagates the v0.7.0 `QuinticHermite` interpolant to `Diffusion4thChernoff`
(K5 base, OPT-IN — default unchanged) and to the ζ-ladder rungs `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff`,
`Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff`, and (Wave II) `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (DEFAULT ON).
Mechanism: each opted-in kernel clones the working `Grid1D` and calls
`.with_interp(InterpKind::QuinticHermite)` before the inner `f.sample(...)`
queries (mirrors `hormander.rs:457` pattern; no new interpolation code).

**Impact on Chernoff kernels** (predicted, to be measured at v4.2-pre):

| Kernel | v4.1 spatial floor (N=512) | v4.2 (Path ε) | Measurable order at N=512 |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Diffusion4thChernoff` (K5 base, opt-in) | ~1.18e-4 (CubicHermite) | ~1e-8 (QuinticHermite) | Spatial 4 unchanged (K-kernel arm count is the limit) |
| `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff` (Richardson, default ON) | 3.55 (calibrated) | ≥ 3.95 (theoretical 4) | Temporal 4 reachable |
| `Diffusion6thChernoff` (γ⁶-A baseline, already ON since v0.7.0) | n/a | n/a | Unchanged from §9.2.6 |
| `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff` (Richardson², default ON) | 3.67 (calibrated) | ≥ 5.8 (theoretical 6) | Temporal 6 reachable |
| `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (Richardson³, NEW Wave II) | n/a (HOLD pending Path ε) | ≥ 6.5 (theoretical 8) | Temporal 8 reachable |

**Backward compatibility (NORMATIVE)**:

- `Grid1D::new(_, _, n)` default UNCHANGED — `InterpKind::CubicHermite`.
- v0.5/v0.6 byte-equality on K5 base: PRESERVED — opt-in only.
- ζ-ladder default behavior change (CubicHermite → QuinticHermite at v4.2 for
  `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff` + `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff`) is documented in
  `docs/migration/v4.1-to-v4.2.md` as bug-fix-grade ("kernel achieves the order
  its `order()` advertises") — not API-breaking.
- Global `Grid1D::new` default promotion (CubicHermite → QuinticHermite) is
  DEFERRED to v5.0 BREAKING window per ADR-0035 §9 deprecation cycles.
- 2D/3D/ND scope (`Grid2D`, `Grid3D`, `GridND`) is OUT OF SCOPE for Path ε;
  per-axis `.with_interp()` is already supported manually.

##### §9.2.6.bis AMENDMENT 1 (2026-05-28 — ADR-0089 AMENDMENT 1) — ζ⁴ default-ON REGRESSION; revert and isolate ζ⁶ wiring

Engineer Wave I measured `g_zeta4_const_a_richardson_ratio` (n-pair {4, 8}, N=512, T=0.5, analytic oracle) returns log₂(ratio) = **3.226** with QuinticHermite default-ON — **DEGRADED** from v4.1 CubicHermite baseline 3.55 (Δ = −0.32); BLOCKING gate at 3.5 FAILS. Companion `g_zeta6_const_a_richardson_ratio` (n-pair {1, 2}) IMPROVED 3.67 → 3.868 (Δ = +0.20). **Mathematical diagnosis**: at n=4 (τ=0.125, pre-asymptotic for the K5+Richardson Galkin-Remizov m=4 specialisation on the T=0.5 horizon), shifting K5's spatial residue from O(dx⁴)·C₄·f⁽⁴⁾ (CubicHermite) to O(dx⁶)·C₆·f⁽⁶⁾ (QuinticHermite) re-orders which higher-order temporal Taylor terms dominate the Richardson `(4·a − b)/3` cancellation; the symmetric K5 odd-power cancellation is no longer the leading effect at this τ-scale. G_zeta6 (n-pair {1, 2}, τ ∈ {0.5, 0.25}) is **insensitive** to this re-ordering because its much larger τ keeps the leading 16/15 Richardson² term dominant regardless of K5 spatial residue shape, while the tightened spatial floor improves the asymptotic floor.

**Decision (AMENDMENT 1)**: Revert `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::new()` to CubicHermite default (mirror K5 base, preserves v0.6/v4.1 byte-equality); keep `.with_quintic_sampling()` as opt-in. `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff::new()` wires K5 Quintic **directly** (bypassing the now-reverted ζ⁴ default) to preserve its 3.868 win. The table at §9.2.6.bis "Impact on Chernoff kernels" is AMENDED:

| Kernel | v4.1 (CubicHermite) | v4.2 (Path ε, AMENDMENT 1) | Measurable order at N=512 |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Diffusion4thChernoff` (K5 base, opt-in) | ~6.5e-7 single-cell midpoint Gaussian | ~7e-9 single-cell midpoint Gaussian | Spatial 4 unchanged |
| `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff` (Richardson, **REVERTED to default OFF**) | 3.55 (calibrated) | 3.55 (preserved; opt-in lifts to TBD) | Temporal asymptotic ~3.5 (full 4 deferred) |
| `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff` (Richardson², default ON via direct K5 Quintic wiring) | 3.67 | 3.868 | Temporal partial 6 (asymptotic ≥ 3.8) |
| `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (Richardson³, Wave II HOLD released) | n/a | TBD (wire K5 Quintic directly, mirror ζ⁶) | Temporal partial 8 |

**Backward compatibility (STRENGTHENED)**: v4.1 byte-equality contract on `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::new()` is now PRESERVED (was bug-fix-grade behavior change in original §9.2.6.bis; now bit-identical). ζ⁶ behavior change CubicHermite→QuinticHermite is bug-fix-grade. ζ⁸ (when Wave II ships) follows the ζ⁶ direct-wiring pattern. Full order-4 for ζ⁴ requires follow-up architect investigation (alternative spatial scheme or n-pair re-calibration) — DEFERRED to v4.3+ ADR-0090. The path_eps_spatial_floor regression test gate semantics shift from K5-stencil floor (1.18e-4) to single-cell-midpoint Catmull-Rom floor (~6.5e-7) per engineer fix; ADR-0089 AMENDMENT 1 §"Regression test fix".

### 9.2.7 — Chebyshev spectral collocation (`InterpKind::ChebyshevSpectral`, NORMATIVE for v4.3, ADR-0090)

> **Status: NORMATIVE for v4.3 release.** Path ε successor; lifts the spatial floor from QuinticHermite ≈ 1e-10 to spectral exponential-accuracy ≤ 1e-15 at N=512, M=64, unblocking ζ⁸ Wave II resurrection (§27.tris).

**Chebyshev-Lobatto nodes** (M+1 nodes on `[−1, 1]`, mapped to `[xmin, xmax]`; NORMATIVE):

$$
y_k = \cos(k\pi / M), \qquad x_k = \tfrac{x_{\max} + x_{\min}}{2} + \tfrac{x_{\max} - x_{\min}}{2}\, y_k, \qquad k = 0, 1, \ldots, M.
$$

Nodes precomputed as `const` arrays for $M \in \{8, 16, 32, 64, 128, 256, 512\}$ in `crates/semiflow-core/src/grid_chebyshev_nodes.rs` (~50 LoC; one-time compile-time cost). Default $M = 64$ per ADR-0090 engineer Wave AC1; configurable via `.with_chebyshev_sampling(m: usize)` builder.

**Barycentric Lagrange interpolation** (Berrut-Trefethen 2004 *SIAM Review* 46:501, formula 5.1; NORMATIVE):

$$
f(x) \;=\; \frac{\displaystyle\sum_{k=0}^{M}\, \frac{w_k\, f_k}{x - x_k}}{\displaystyle\sum_{k=0}^{M}\, \frac{w_k}{x - x_k}}, \qquad
w_k = (-1)^k \, \delta_k, \qquad \delta_0 = \delta_M = \tfrac{1}{2},\; \delta_k = 1 \;(\text{else}),
$$

with the convention $f(x_k) = f_k$ at the nodes (the singularity at $x = x_k$ is removable; engineer implementation returns $f_k$ exactly when $|x - x_k| < $ ULP).

**Virtual-node construction (NORMATIVE for v4.3 opt-in)**: each call `Grid1D::interp(values, x)` with `InterpKind::ChebyshevSpectral` first computes the M+1 virtual node values $f_k \,{=}\, \mathrm{sample\_quintic\_1d}(\text{values}, \text{\&grid}, x_k)$ from the underlying uniform-grid `values: &[f64]` using the existing `grid_quintic.rs` machinery (§9.2.6). The barycentric formula above then delivers the spectral-accurate evaluation at `x`. Per-sample cost: $O(M)$ QuinticHermite evals + $O(M)$ barycentric ops = $\approx 2M$ floating-point operations; at $M = 64$ this is ≈ 128 flops, comparable to a single 4-point Catmull-Rom cell sample plus its 4 BC lookups.

**Spatial floor (asymptotic, NORMATIVE)**: for smooth $f$ analytic in a strip of half-width $\gamma > 0$ around $[-1, 1]$, Chebyshev tail truncation gives

$$
\bigl| f(x) - f_M(x) \bigr| \;\le\; C \cdot e^{-\gamma M},
$$

where $f_M$ is the degree-$M$ Chebyshev interpolant. For the canonical Gaussian probe $f(x) = e^{-x^2}$ on $[-10, 10]$ with $\gamma \approx 1$, $M = 64$ gives $e^{-64} \approx 10^{-28}$ — far below the virtual-node QuinticHermite floor $\sim$ 1e-10. **Effective spatial floor** $\;=\; \max(\text{QuinticHermite virtual-node floor},\ \text{Chebyshev tail},\ \text{f64 ULP}) \;\approx\; 1\text{e-}10$ for the default 6-point FD ghost-data construction. To reach the $G_\text{PATH\_EPS\_CHEB\_FLOOR} \le 10^{-15}$ acceptance gate, the engineer Wave MUST EITHER (a) extend `grid_quintic::fd_scaled_prime` from the current 6-point central FD ($O(dx^7)$ on scaled derivative) to a 10-point or 12-point variant ($O(dx^{11}) / O(dx^{13})$), pushing the virtual-node floor below $10^{-15}$, OR (b) use the closed-form analytic Greville construction (Boyd 1989 Ch. 17) at virtual nodes for the regression-gate Gaussian probe specifically. Engineer chooses at AC1-AC2 time; documented in `.dev-docs/specs/chebyshev-wave.md` §"Risk".

**Differentiation matrix (CITATION, NORMATIVE for any future direct spectral derivative)**: the dense $D_M \in \mathbb{R}^{(M+1)\times(M+1)}$ that maps nodal values to nodal first derivatives is tabulated in Trefethen 2000 *Spectral Methods in MATLAB* (SIAM), Differentiation Matrix Appendix, formula A.5:

$$
(D_M)_{ij} = \begin{cases}
\dfrac{c_i}{c_j}\,\dfrac{(-1)^{i+j}}{y_i - y_j}, & i \ne j, \\[6pt]
-\dfrac{y_i}{2(1 - y_i^2)}, & 1 \le i = j \le M-1, \\[6pt]
\dfrac{2M^2 + 1}{6}, & i = j = 0, \\[6pt]
-\dfrac{2M^2 + 1}{6}, & i = j = M,
\end{cases} \qquad c_0 = c_M = 2,\; c_k = 1\ (\text{else}).
$$

v4.3 does NOT use $D_M$ directly (the kernels apply Chernoff functions, not raw spectral derivatives); $D_M$ is documented here for v4.4+ optional kernels (e.g. a future `Diffusion10thChebyshevChernoff` that bypasses Richardson cascade entirely).

**Backward compatibility (NORMATIVE)**:

- `InterpKind::ChebyshevSpectral` is a NEW variant added to the `InterpKind` enum in `boundary.rs` alongside `CubicHermite` / `Linear` / `QuinticHermite` (additive; existing variants unchanged).
- `Grid1D::new` default UNCHANGED — `CubicHermite`.
- v4.2 ζ-ladder defaults UNCHANGED — `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::new` stays CubicHermite (per ADR-0089 AMENDMENT 1); `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff::new` stays QuinticHermite via direct K5 wiring.
- Per-kernel Chebyshev opt-in is OFF by default on K5 base, ζ⁴, ζ⁶; opt in via `.with_chebyshev_sampling()` (optionally `.with_chebyshev_sampling_m(m: usize)` for non-default M).
- `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (NEW Wave II resurrection per §27.tris) defaults Chebyshev ON — its `order()` contract IS 8, and only spectral floor can demonstrate it.
- `f32` / `SemiflowComplex` callers of opted-in kernels: `SemiflowError::Unsupported { feature: "ChebyshevSpectral is f64-only in v4.3" }` (mirrors QuinticHermite f64-only constraint at `grid.rs:196-198`).
- Global `Grid1D::new` default promotion to `ChebyshevSpectral` is DEFERRED to v5.0 BREAKING window per ADR-0035 §9.
- 2D/3D/ND (`Grid2D`, `Grid3D`, `GridND`) tensor-product Chebyshev OUT OF SCOPE for v4.3.

#### §9.2.7 v4.6 PREP-MEASUREMENT footnote (ADR-0097, B.3 re-measurement campaign)

The v4.3 Chebyshev opt-in (`.with_chebyshev_sampling()`) shipped per ADR-0090 Wave A WITHOUT measuring the resulting ζ⁴/ζ⁶ Richardson ratios under the new spatial sample. The v4.3 calibration `G_zeta6_const_a_richardson = 3.868` (ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 1; QuinticHermite-bound asymptote) remains the operative gate at v4.3+; the Chebyshev opt-in is verified ONLY by `G_zeta8_const_a_richardson_cheb = 6.5` (ADR-0090) and the spectral floor regression gate `G_PATH_EPS_CHEB_FLOOR ≤ 10^{-15}`. The v4.6.0 PREP-MEASUREMENT MINOR release per ADR-0097 closes this measurement gap by adding 4 new sibling gates (`G_zeta{4,6}_{const_a_richardson,var_a_slope}_cheb`), each calibrated per the Option E hybrid rule `threshold = \lfloor \text{measured} - 0.1 \rfloor + 0.1` (ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1). Expected post-calibration: `G_zeta6_const_a_richardson_cheb ≥ 5.5` (recovers from QuinticHermite-bound 3.868 toward theoretical 6) and `G_zeta4_const_a_richardson_cheb ≥ 3.9` (recovers from CubicHermite-default 3.55 baseline; ADR-0089 AMENDMENT 1 §"Chebyshev removes higher-order Taylor re-ordering"). The B.3 verdict (GREEN/AMBER/RED) governs the v5.0 BREAKING decision on global `Grid1D::new` default promotion `CubicHermite → ChebyshevSpectral { m: 64 }` (ADR-0099 PENDING; conditional on B.3 ≠ RED). See `.dev-docs/reports/V4_6_B3_REMEASURE_REPORT.md` for the measurement record post-Wave.

### 9.3 Drift-reaction Chernoff `R(τ)` — RK2 characteristics (v0.2.2)

For $B = b(x)\partial_x + c(x)$ acting on the linear PDE
$\partial_t u = b(x)\,\partial_x u + c(x)\,u$ with $u(0,x) = f(x)$, the exact
solution along characteristics $\dot{X}(s) = -b(X(s))$ traced backward from
$(τ, x)$ to $(0, X(τ, x))$ is

$$
u(\tau, x) \;=\; \exp\!\Big(\!\int_0^\tau c\!\big(X(s, x)\big)\,\mathrm{d}s\Big)\,
                 f\!\big(X(\tau, x)\big),
$$

with the convention that $X(s, x)$ is the foot-point at time $0$ of the
characteristic ending at the space-time point $(τ, x)$ (the "value at $(τ,x)$
originates from $X(τ,x)$"). Substituting $\sigma = -s$ in the characteristic
ODE shows $X$ satisfies the *forward* drift ODE
$\partial_\tau X(\tau, x) = b\!\big(X(\tau, x)\big)$, $X(0, x) = x$. **In
particular, the foot-point shift is positive in $b$**: for constant $b$,
$X(\tau, x) = x + \tau b$ and the value at $(\tau, x)$ comes from $x + \tau b$,
matching the v0.2.1 closed-form sign $f(x + \tau\,b)$.

#### v0.2.2 formula — RK2 (midpoint + trapezoidal)

The v0.2.2 implementation evaluates the characteristic foot-point with the
classical **midpoint (RK2) rule** and the reaction-integral with the
**trapezoidal rule**:

$$
\boxed{\;
\begin{aligned}
X(\tau, x) \;&:=\; x \;+\; \tau\,b\!\Big(x + \tfrac{\tau}{2}\,b(x)\Big), \\[4pt]
\big(R(\tau)\,f\big)(x) \;&:=\;
  \exp\!\Big(\tfrac{\tau}{2}\,\big(c(x) + c\!\big(X(\tau, x)\big)\big)\Big)
  \cdot f\!\big(X(\tau, x)\big).
\end{aligned}
\;}
$$

**Sign convention**: the shift inside $f$ is **PLUS**, identical to v0.2.1
(`drift_reaction.rs` module doc; verified: $\partial_\tau f(x + \tau b)\big|_{\tau=0}
= b\,f'(x) = b\,\partial_x f(x)$ ✓). The midpoint slope $b\big(x + (τ/2)b(x)\big)$
is evaluated at the *forward Euler half-step*, consistent with $\dot{X} = b(X)$.

#### Order claim

For $b \in C^2(\mathbb{R})$, $c \in C^1(\mathbb{R})$ both bounded with bounded
derivatives,

$$
\big(R(\tau) f\big)(x) \;-\; u(\tau, x) \;=\; O(\tau^3) \quad\text{(local)},
$$

and the iterated approximant $\big(R(\tau)\big)^n$ over $n = T/\tau$ steps has
**global error $O(\tau^2)$**, by the standard Chernoff-product theorem
(§2 + Hairer–Lubich–Wanner §III.5). Algebraic verification is in
`.dev-docs/verification/variable-drift-rk2-derivation.md` §2–§4.

#### Reduction-to-constant lemma (regression-safety)

**Claim.** When $b$ and $c$ are **constants** ($b(x) \equiv b_0$, $c(x) \equiv c_0$),
the v0.2.2 RK2 formula collapses *exactly* (no $O(\tau^3)$ slack — bit-equal
modulo IEEE rounding of the same arithmetic) to the v0.2.1 closed form
$e^{\tau c_0}\,f(x + \tau b_0)$:

- **Midpoint foot-point.** For constant $b \equiv b_0$,
  $b\big(x + (\tau/2)\,b_0\big) = b_0$, hence
  $X(\tau, x) = x + \tau b_0$ — *exact* (this is the exact characteristic
  for constant $b$, so RK2 has zero truncation error in this regime).
- **Trapezoidal reaction.** For constant $c \equiv c_0$,
  $\tfrac{\tau}{2}(c_0 + c_0) = \tau c_0$ — *exact*.
- **Combined.** $R(\tau) f(x) = e^{\tau c_0}\,f(x + \tau b_0)$ — bit-equal to
  v0.2.1 modulo the `(τ/2)*c0 + (τ/2)*c0` vs `τ*c0` rearrangement (one extra
  add, no precision loss to within a few ULPs).

**Consequence.** v0.2.0 acceptance gates G1, G2, G3-strang, G4-strang (§6.2)
all use constant coefficients $\alpha = \beta = 1/2$, $c \equiv 0$, so the
upgrade introduces *no* numerical change at any test point of those gates
beyond floating-point rearrangement noise (bounded by ≈ 4 ULPs per
evaluation; well below the gate thresholds $1\!\times\!10^{-4}$,
$1\!\times\!10^{-6}$, slope tolerance $0.05$). G1-legacy / G2-legacy
(heat kernel, $b = 0$) are equally unaffected. **The upgrade is
regression-safe by construction.** Property
`drift_reaction_constant_fast_path_exact` (properties.yaml) enforces this
empirically over 1000 random $(b_0, c_0, \tau)$ triples to tolerance
$1\!\times\!10^{-13}$.

#### Variable-coefficient oracle (linear-restoring drift)

To exercise the v0.2.2 order-2 lift directly the contract designates the
following manufactured-solution oracle:

$$
b(x) \;=\; -\gamma\,x, \qquad c(x) \;\equiv\; -\kappa\gamma \quad
(\gamma > 0,\ \kappa \in \mathbb{R}),
$$

i.e., a linear restoring drift toward $x = 0$ with constant reaction.
The characteristic ODE $\dot{X} = -\gamma X$ has the closed form
$X(\tau, x) = x\,e^{-\gamma\tau}$ (forward $\tau$-flow of $b$ in the
sign convention above), and the reaction integral is constant
$\int_0^\tau c \mathrm{d}s = -\kappa\gamma\tau$. For Gaussian initial data
$f(x) = \exp\!\big(-x^2/(2\sigma^2)\big)$ the exact solution at time $\tau$ is

$$
\boxed{\;
u(\tau, x) \;=\;
  \exp(-\kappa\gamma\tau)\,\exp\!\Big(\!-\,\frac{x^2\,e^{-2\gamma\tau}}{2\sigma^2}\Big).
\;}
$$

(Substitute $X(\tau, x) = x\,e^{-\gamma\tau}$ into $f(X(\tau, x))$ and multiply
by $e^{-\kappa\gamma\tau}$.) Property `drift_reaction_variable_order2`
(properties.yaml) sweeps $(\tau, \gamma, \kappa, \sigma)$ over 200 cases and
verifies log-log slope $\le -1.95$ in $\tau$ at fixed $\gamma$. The $\tanh$
drift originally floated (e.g., $b(x) = \beta\tanh(\gamma x)$) is rejected
because $\dot{X} = -\beta\tanh(\gamma X)$ has no closed-form solution in
elementary functions — the linear restoring drift is the simplest variable-$b$
PDE with a tractable analytic oracle. The full algebra is in
`.dev-docs/verification/variable-drift-rk2-derivation.md` §6.

#### Strang-composition order preservation (cross-ref §9.7)

`StrangSplit<DiffusionChernoff, DriftReactionChernoff>` retains its global
$O(\tau^2)$ guarantee under the v0.2.2 upgrade for both regimes:

- **Constant coefficients** (the v0.2.0 production oracle, §6.2 / §9.7). The
  reduction lemma above shows $R$ is bit-identical to the v0.2.1 exact form,
  so §9.7's analysis (commutator $[A, B] = 0$, $\Phi(\tau) = D(\tau/2)^2 \cdot
  e^{\tau B}$, slope $= -2$ from $D$'s local $O(\tau^3)$) applies verbatim.
- **Variable coefficients** ($v$0.3+, formally enabled by this upgrade). The
  inner $R$ now has local $O(\tau^3)$ and is *time-symmetric* in the sense of
  the trapezoidal-rule symmetry $c(x_0) + c(x_1)$. Combined with $D$'s local
  $O(\tau^3)$ and the palindromic Strang structure (Hairer–Lubich–Wanner
  §III.5, Thm 4.1), the leading $\tau^3$ commutator term cancels and the
  global error remains $O(\tau^2)$ — re-derivation **not** required for
  $v$0.2.2; this is the canonical Strang result invoked here as a forward
  reference for $v$0.3+.

### 9.4 Strang composition

$$
\boxed{\;
\Phi(\tau)\;:=\;D(\tau/2)\,\circ\,R(\tau)\,\circ\,D(\tau/2).
\;}
$$

For constant $(a, b, c)$ — the test-oracle regime — $[A, B] = 0$ gives
$e^{\tau(A+B)} = e^{\tau A}\,e^{\tau B}$ exactly. With $R$ exact and $D(\tau)$
having local error $O(\tau^3)$:

$$
\Phi(\tau) - e^{\tau L}
\;=\;
\big(D(\tau/2) - e^{(\tau/2)A}\big)\,e^{\tau B}\,e^{(\tau/2)A}
\;+\; e^{(\tau/2)A}\,e^{\tau B}\,\big(D(\tau/2) - e^{(\tau/2)A}\big)
\;+\; O(\tau^4)
\;=\; O(\tau^3),
$$

where each $D(\tau/2) - e^{(\tau/2)A} = O((\tau/2)^3)$. **Per-step error:
$O(\tau^3)$. Global error over $n = T/\tau$ steps: $n \cdot O(\tau^3) = O(\tau^2)$**.
This justifies the G3-strang gate (slope $\le -1.95$ leaves $0.05$ margin
for grid-discretization and pre-asymptotic effects).

For variable coefficients ($[A,B] \ne 0$), the palindromic structure of
Strang causes the leading $\tau^3$ term in the BCH expansion of $\Phi$ to
match the corresponding term in $e^{\tau(A+B)}$, preserving global $O(\tau^2)$
(canonical result; see Hairer–Lubich–Wanner §III.5.4).

### 9.5 Advection-diffusion oracle (G1, G2, G3-strang)

Equation: $\partial_t u = \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_{xx} u + \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x u$,
$u(0, x) = e^{-x^2}$. Substitute $v(t, y) := u(t, y - \beta t)$ with $\beta = 1/2$:

$$
\partial_t v \;=\; \partial_t u(t, y - \beta t) - \beta\,\partial_x u(t, y - \beta t)
\;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_{xx} u + \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x u - \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x u
\;=\; \tfrac{1}{2}\partial_{yy} v,
$$

with $v(0, y) = u(0, y) = e^{-y^2}$. Pure heat equation with $\alpha = 1/2$;
classical solution

$$
v(t, y) = (1 + 2 t)^{-1/2}\,\exp\!\Big(-\frac{y^2}{1 + 2 t}\Big).
$$

Inverting the substitution ($u(t, x) = v(t, x + \beta t) = v(t, x + t/2)$):

$$
\boxed{\;
u(t, x) \;=\; (1 + 2 t)^{-1/2}\,\exp\!\Big(-\frac{(x + t/2)^2}{1 + 2 t}\Big).
\;}
$$

At $t = 1$: $u(1, x) = 3^{-1/2}\,\exp(-(x + 0.5)^2 / 3)$. Mass-centre
translation $0 \to -0.5$ confirms $B$ step is non-trivial.

### 9.6 Quasi-contractivity (G4-strang invariant)

$D(\tau)$ has positive weights summing to 1, so $\|D(\tau) f\|_\infty \le \|f\|_\infty$.
$R(\tau)$ multiplies by $e^{\tau c(x)}$ pointwise, so
$\|R(\tau) f\|_\infty \le e^{\tau \|c\|_\infty}\|f\|_\infty$. Composing
the Strang sandwich:

$$
\|\Phi(\tau) f\|_\infty \;\le\; 1 \cdot e^{\tau \|c\|_\infty} \cdot 1 \cdot \|f\|_\infty
\;=\; e^{\tau \|c\|_\infty}\,\|f\|_\infty
\;\le\; \big(1 + \|c\|_\infty\,\tau + \tfrac{(\|c\|_\infty\,\tau)^2}{2}\,e^{\|c\|_\infty\,\tau}\big)\,\|f\|_\infty.
$$

For the proptest range $\|c\|_\infty \le 5$ and $\tau \le 0.1$, the $\tau^2$
coefficient $\tfrac{\|c\|^2}{2}\,e^{\|c\|\tau} \le \tfrac{25}{2}\,e^{0.5} \approx 20.6$;
absorbing interpolation overshoot the safe constant is $C = 20$:

$$
\boxed{\;
\|\Phi(\tau) f\|_\infty \;\le\; \big(1 + |c|\,\tau + 20\,\tau^2\big)\,\|f\|_\infty
\quad \text{for } \tau \in (0, 0.1],\ \|c\|_\infty \le 5.
\;}
$$

This is the G4-strang invariant, exercised by 10 000 proptest cases.

### 9.7 Spatial-error budget for `StrangSplit` (2026-04-29 amendments 3 + 4)

#### Two empirical anchor measurements

Two QA executions provide anchor measurements of $\|u_{\text{cher}} - u_{\text{oracle}}\|_\infty$
on $\Omega = [-10, 10]$, $\alpha = \beta = 0.5,\ c = 0$, `Reflect` BC,
`CubicHermite` interp:

**Anchor A** ($N = 1000$, pre-amendment-3 measurement):

| $n$  | err at $N=1000$ |
|------|-----------------|
| 32   | $3.12 \times 10^{-6}$ |
| 64   | $2.27 \times 10^{-6}$ |
| 128  | $7.16 \times 10^{-6}$ |
| 256  | $1.06 \times 10^{-5}$ |
| 512  | $1.25 \times 10^{-5}$ |
| 1024 | $1.38 \times 10^{-5}$ |

**Anchor B** ($N = 8000$, post-amendment-3 measurement):

| $n$  | err at $N=8000$ |
|------|-----------------|
| 32   | $2.65 \times 10^{-6}$ |
| 64   | $6.58 \times 10^{-7}$ |
| 128  | $1.65 \times 10^{-7}$ |
| 256  | $5.11 \times 10^{-8}$ |
| 512  | $3.36 \times 10^{-8}$ |
| 1024 | $1.12 \times 10^{-7}$ (rebound) |

Anchor B's slope on all 6 points is $-1.07$, but on the first 4 points
($n \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}$) it is $-1.91$ — clean order-2 in the
time-dominated regime. The rebound between $n = 512$ and $n = 1024$
(error grows by $\sim 3.3\times$) is *not* consistent with a static
spatial floor (which would plateau at the time/space crossover).

#### Why Amendment-3's $\Delta x^4$ floor model was wrong

Cross-validating the floor at $n = 1024$ between the two anchors:

$$
\frac{\text{floor}(1024, N{=}1000)}{\text{floor}(1024, N{=}8000)}
\;\approx\;
\frac{1.38\times 10^{-5}}{1.12\times 10^{-7}}
\;\approx\; 124.
$$

The grid ratio $N{=}8000 / N{=}1000 = 8$. If the floor scaled as $\Delta x^4$
the ratio would be $8^4 = 4096$ — *not* $124$. Solving
$8^p = 124$ gives $p = \log 124 / \log 8 \approx 2.32$. Hence the floor
empirically scales as $\Delta x^{2.32}$, not $\Delta x^4$.

#### Why the floor grows linearly in $n$ at fixed $N$

At $N = 8000$, $\Delta x = 2.5\times 10^{-3}$. The drift shift per Strang
step is $\tau\beta = (T\beta)/n = 0.5/n$. The crossover where
$\tau\beta = \Delta x$ occurs at $n^\star = T\beta / \Delta x = 200$.
For $n > n^\star$, the drift shift falls *sub-grid*; the cubic-Hermite
kernel must interpolate at very small fractional shifts, and per-step
errors accumulate linearly across the $n$-step iteration without full
cancellation in the palindromic Strang sandwich:

| $n$  | $\tau\beta$ at $N=8000$ | $\tau\beta / \Delta x$ |
|------|-------------------------|------------------------|
| 32   | $1.56\times 10^{-2}$    | $6.25$  (super-grid)   |
| 64   | $7.81\times 10^{-3}$    | $3.13$  (super-grid)   |
| 128  | $3.91\times 10^{-3}$    | $1.56$  (super-grid)   |
| 256  | $1.95\times 10^{-3}$    | $0.78$  (sub-grid)     |
| 512  | $9.77\times 10^{-4}$    | $0.39$  (sub-grid)     |
| 1024 | $4.88\times 10^{-4}$    | $0.20$  (deep sub-grid) |

Anchor B's transition from clean order-2 ($n \le 256$) to floor-dominated
($n \ge 512$) coincides with this drift-shift crossover, confirming the
mechanism. *Note*: the diffusion shifts $h = 2\sqrt{\alpha\tau}$,
$H = 2\sqrt{3\alpha\tau}$ remain super-grid throughout the slope window
($h/\Delta x \ge 17.7$ at $N = 8000$, $n = 1024$), so the diffusion
half-steps are not the source of the floor.

#### Calibrated empirical model (Amendment-4)

$$
\boxed{\;
\text{err}(n, N)
\;\approx\;
\sqrt{\Big(\frac{C_t}{n^2}\Big)^2
\;+\;\big(K \cdot n \cdot \Delta x^p\big)^2},
\qquad
\Delta x \;=\; \frac{20}{N - 1},
\;}
$$

with parameters fit from anchors A and B:

$$
C_t \;\approx\; 2.7\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
K \;\approx\; 1.17\times 10^{-4},
\qquad
p \;\approx\; 2.32.
$$

$C_t$ is calibrated from the time-dominated point $(n, N) = (32, 8000)$:
$C_t = 2.65\times 10^{-6} \cdot 32^2 \approx 2.7\times 10^{-3}$. $K$ and $p$
are jointly determined by the floor-dominated point $(1024, 1000)$ and
$(1024, 8000)$.

**Per-point fit at $N = 8000$**:

| $n$  | actual              | model               | actual / model |
|------|---------------------|---------------------|----------------|
| 32   | $2.65\times 10^{-6}$ | $2.65\times 10^{-6}$ | $1.00$         |
| 64   | $6.58\times 10^{-7}$ | $6.64\times 10^{-7}$ | $0.99$         |
| 128  | $1.65\times 10^{-7}$ | $1.66\times 10^{-7}$ | $0.99$         |
| 256  | $5.11\times 10^{-8}$ | $5.00\times 10^{-8}$ | $1.02$         |
| 512  | $3.36\times 10^{-8}$ | $5.66\times 10^{-8}$ | $0.59$ (model conservative) |
| 1024 | $1.12\times 10^{-7}$ | $1.11\times 10^{-7}$ | $1.00$         |

The model is conservative at $n = 512$ (predicts higher error than
observed; the actual smoothing at the time-floor crossover is gentler
than the orthogonal-RSS model assumes). The model fits the slope-driving
points (low and high $n$) within ratio 1.0; the systematic conservatism
biases the predicted slope to be *less* negative than the actual slope —
i.e., real measurements should always be a little better than the
model's prediction.

**Time-constant interpretation.** $C_t \approx 2.7\times 10^{-3}$
empirically realises the global-$O(\tau^2)$ envelope of §9.4. From
§9.2, the leading symbol error of $D(\tau)$ is $\frac{1}{30}(\alpha\tau)^3 \xi^6$;
applied to the $t = 1$ Gaussian profile (whose $\|u^{(VI)}\|_\infty$
is bounded), the per-step $O(\tau^3)$ accumulates over $n$ steps to give
$\sim n \cdot \tau^3 = T\,\tau^2 = T / n^2$ in the global envelope. The
empirical $C_t$ is consistent with this scaling; the smaller-than-naive
constant reflects partial cancellation in the palindromic Strang
composition.

#### Required $N$ for G3-strang slope $\le -1.95$

We need the floor at $n = 1024$ to be at least a factor $\sim 5\text{-}10$
below the time error $C_t / 1024^2 \approx 2.6 \times 10^{-9}$, so the
log-log regression on the 6-point grid is dominated by the time trend
rather than the floor tail. With the calibrated model:

$$
K \cdot 1024 \cdot \Delta x^p
\;\le\; \frac{1}{F} \cdot \frac{C_t}{1024^2}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\Delta x \;\le\; \left(\frac{C_t}{K \cdot 1024^3 \cdot F}\right)^{1/p}.
$$

For $F = 8$ and $p = 2.32$: $\Delta x \le 2.0 \times 10^{-4}$, hence
$N \ge 1 + 20 / 2.0\times 10^{-4} = 100001$. Round to **$N = 100000$**.

Predictions across candidate $N$ (under the combined model above):

| $N$       | $\Delta x$           | floor at $n=1024$       | predicted slope | G1 ($n=100$)         | G2 ($n=1000$)        |
|-----------|----------------------|-------------------------|-----------------|----------------------|----------------------|
| 1000      | $2.00\times 10^{-2}$ | $1.4\times 10^{-5}$     | $+0.2$ (FAIL)   | $\sim 10^{-5}$       | $\sim 10^{-5}$ (FAIL) |
| 8000      | $2.50\times 10^{-3}$ | $1.1\times 10^{-7}$     | $-1.01$ (FAIL)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $1.1\times 10^{-7}$ (FAIL by 100×) |
| 16000     | $1.25\times 10^{-3}$ | $2.2\times 10^{-8}$     | $-1.51$ (FAIL)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $2.2\times 10^{-8}$  |
| 32000     | $6.25\times 10^{-4}$ | $4.5\times 10^{-9}$     | $-1.85$ (FAIL)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $5.2\times 10^{-9}$  |
| 50000     | $4.00\times 10^{-4}$ | $1.6\times 10^{-9}$     | $-1.97$ (PASS)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $3.1\times 10^{-9}$  |
| 80000     | $2.50\times 10^{-4}$ | $5.4\times 10^{-10}$    | $-2.00$ (PASS)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $2.8\times 10^{-9}$  |
| **100000** | **$2.00\times 10^{-4}$** | **$3.2\times 10^{-10}$** | **$-2.00$ (PASS)** | **$2.7\times 10^{-7}$** | **$2.7\times 10^{-9}$** |
| 160000    | $1.25\times 10^{-4}$ | $1.1\times 10^{-10}$    | $-2.00$ (PASS)  | $2.7\times 10^{-7}$  | $2.7\times 10^{-9}$  |

(Predicted slope values are reported to three decimals in the analysis
script; this table rounds to two for readability. $-2.00$ rounds from
$-1.998$ at $N = 100000$.)

#### Sensitivity to the floor exponent $p$

The exponent $p \approx 2.32$ is calibrated from only two anchor points.
A robust choice of $N$ should clear the gate even under adversarial
deviation in $p$:

| $p$  | predicted slope at $N = 80000$ | predicted slope at $N = 100000$ |
|------|--------------------------------|---------------------------------|
| 1.5  | $-1.890$ (FAIL — implausible $p$) | $-1.930$ (FAIL) |
| 2.0  | $-1.982$ (PASS) | $-1.989$ (PASS) |
| 2.32 | $-1.996$ (PASS) | $-1.998$ (PASS) |
| 2.5  | $-1.998$ (PASS) | $-1.999$ (PASS) |
| 3.0  | $-2.000$ (PASS) | $-2.000$ (PASS) |
| 4.0  | $-2.000$ (PASS) | $-2.000$ (PASS) |

For $p \ge 2.0$, $N = 100000$ clears the gate by $\ge 0.039$. The
$p = 1.5$ case would imply the cubic-Hermite kernel is providing only
$\sim 1.5$-order accuracy in the dx limit, which contradicts its
canonical 4th-order accuracy theorem (Catmull-Rom on a uniform grid
reproduces cubics exactly); we therefore treat $p \ge 2.0$ as the
defensible regime and $p = 1.5$ as a strict pessimum. **Choosing
$N = 100000$ defends the gate over the entire defensible range of $p$.**

#### Why this is *not* a gate relaxation

The acceptance gates ($1\times 10^{-4}$, $1\times 10^{-6}$,
slope $\le -1.95$, proptest constant $20$) are **unchanged**. Only the
*grid-resolution harness parameter* $N$ is updated, and the update is
calibrated against measured data, not estimated under the prior
incorrect $\Delta x^4$ assumption. The original $N = 8000$ was chosen
under a model that empirically over-estimated the spatial floor's
$\Delta x$-sensitivity by a factor of $\sim 30$ at the relevant $n$
window; the corrected $N = 100000$ is the smallest engineering-friendly
round value that defends the slope gate under all defensible
$p$-sensitivities. The empirical model for $C_t$ and $K$ is independent
of $N$ (it is calibrated jointly across two anchors with different $N$),
so the prediction at $N = 100000$ is a forward extrapolation of the
verified physics rather than a hopeful guess.

#### Constant-coefficient regime: what the slope actually tests

For the test oracle ($\alpha = \beta = 0.5,\ c = 0$, all constant) the
diffusion–drift commutator $[A, B] = a\beta\,[\partial_{xx}, \partial_x]
+ a\,[\partial_{xx}, c\cdot] = 0$. Since $D(\tau/2)$ is a function of $A$
only and $e^{\tau B}$ commutes with $A$:

$$
\Phi(\tau) \;=\; D(\tau/2)\,e^{\tau B}\,D(\tau/2) \;=\; D(\tau/2)^2\,e^{\tau B},
\qquad
e^{\tau L} \;=\; e^{\tau A}\,e^{\tau B},
$$

so $\Phi(\tau) - e^{\tau L} = (D(\tau/2)^2 - e^{\tau A})\,e^{\tau B}$.
With $D(\tau/2) = e^{(\tau/2) A} + O(\tau^3)$:
$D(\tau/2)^2 = e^{\tau A} + O(\tau^3)$. **Per-step $O(\tau^3)$, global
$O(\tau^2)$ — slope $-2$.** The order-2 lift in this regime comes purely
from the local $O(\tau^3)$ accuracy of the 5-point $D$, not from
BCH-commutator cancellation in Strang. The test therefore exercises
(i) the algebraic correctness of $D$'s weights, (ii) Strang
state-threading, and (iii) the interpolation kernel on a moving
Gaussian — all the v0.2.0 production-critical pieces. Variable-coefficient
testing (where Strang's palindromic structure cancels the leading
commutator) is deferred to **v0.3+** (technical-constraints.md R6) and
will require a different oracle.

---

## 10. Tensor-product 2D extension (v0.5.0, ADR-0012)

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.5.0. Anchors the forward-reference at §9.2.3.B
(line 1463-1464):

> "The 2D tensor-product extension $\Phi^{2D}$ inherits the same per-axis
> order-2 result."

This section provides the theorem and proof sketch that justify the Phase 1
contracts in `contracts/semiflow-core.tensor.yaml`. Phase 2 implementation
ships against those contracts.

### 10.1 Setting

Let $L_x: \mathcal{D}(L_x) \subset L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_x) \to L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_x)$
and $L_y: \mathcal{D}(L_y) \subset L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_y) \to L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_y)$
be 1D generators of strongly continuous semigroups $e^{tL_x}$ and $e^{tL_y}$,
each satisfying the Theorem 6 hypotheses (§1) on its respective real line.
On the tensor-product domain $\mathcal{D}(L_x) \otimes \mathcal{D}(L_y)$
define the **separable 2D generator**

$$
L \;:=\; L_x \otimes I_y \;+\; I_x \otimes L_y,
$$

acting on functions $f: \mathbb{R}_x \times \mathbb{R}_y \to \mathbb{R}$
in (the closure of) $C_c^\infty(\mathbb{R}^2)$ as

$$
(L f)(x, y) \;=\; (L_x f(\cdot, y))(x) \;+\; (L_y f(x, \cdot))(y).
$$

**Discrete realisation.** For Phase 1 contracts, $f$ is sampled on the
rectangular grid $G^{2D} = G_x \times G_y$ with $|G_x| = n_x$ and
$|G_y| = n_y$, stored as a single `Vec<f64>` of length $n_x \cdot n_y$ in
row-major order with linear index

$$
\mathrm{idx}(i, j) \;:=\; j \cdot n_x + i, \qquad i \in [0, n_x),\ j \in [0, n_y).
$$

(x is the fast axis; this matches the C / NumPy "C-contiguous" convention
and makes X-rows contiguous.)

### 10.2 Lifted Chernoff functions

Let $\Phi_x: [0, T] \to L(L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_x))$ and
$\Phi_y: [0, T] \to L(L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_y))$ be 1D Chernoff functions
satisfying the Theorem 6 hypotheses (§1) for $L_x$ and $L_y$ respectively
(both order $m \ge 1$ on a common core, both quasi-contractive).

Define their **axis-lifts** acting on $f: \mathbb{R}_x \times \mathbb{R}_y \to \mathbb{R}$ by

$$
(\widetilde{\Phi}_x(\tau) f)(x, y) \;:=\; \bigl(\Phi_x(\tau)\, f(\cdot, y)\bigr)(x),
\qquad
(\widetilde{\Phi}_y(\tau) f)(x, y) \;:=\; \bigl(\Phi_y(\tau)\, f(x, \cdot)\bigr)(y).
$$

The discrete realisations are `AxisLift<X>` and `AxisLift<Y>` (see
`tensor.yaml`): apply $\Phi_x$ row-by-row at fixed $j \in [0, n_y)$, and
$\Phi_y$ column-by-column at fixed $i \in [0, n_x)$.

**The 2D Chernoff function** is the palindromic Strang composition

$$
\boxed{\;
\Phi^{2D}(\tau, f)(x, y) \;:=\; \widetilde{\Phi}_x(\tau/2)\,
                                 \widetilde{\Phi}_y(\tau)\,
                                 \widetilde{\Phi}_x(\tau/2)\, f(x, y).
\;}
\qquad (10.1)
$$

In contracts: `Strang2D<X, Y>` carries `x: AxisLift<X, Axis::X>` and
`y: AxisLift<Y, Axis::Y>`; its `apply` invokes them in the order $(x, y, x)$
with half-step on the outer two.

### 10.3 Theorem 7 (per-axis order-2 lift for separable $L$)

**Theorem 7.** *Suppose:*

*(H1) $L = L_x \otimes I + I \otimes L_y$ is separable.*

*(H2) $\Phi_x, \Phi_y$ are 1D Chernoff functions for $L_x, L_y$ each*
*generating $e^{tL_x}, e^{tL_y}$ in the strong topology of*
*$L^\infty$ with order $m \ge 2$ (i.e., 1D global error*
*$\|(\Phi_\bullet(\tau))^n g - e^{nt L_\bullet} g\|_\infty = O(\tau^2)$*
*for fixed $T = n\tau$).*

*(H3) $\Phi_x, \Phi_y$ are quasi-contractive: $\|\Phi_\bullet(\tau)\| \le M_\bullet e^{\omega_\bullet \tau}$.*

*Then the iterated 2D approximant $(\Phi^{2D}(t/n))^n f$ converges to*
*$e^{tL}f$ as $n \to \infty$, for every $f \in C_c^\infty(\mathbb{R}^2)$,*
*with global sup-norm error*

$$
\bigl\| (\Phi^{2D}(t/n))^n f \;-\; e^{tL} f \bigr\|_\infty
\;=\; O(\tau^2), \qquad \tau = t/n.
\qquad (10.2)
$$

**Proof sketch.**

**Step 1 — separability ⇒ commutator vanishes.** For all $\varphi \in
\mathcal{D}(L_x) \otimes \mathcal{D}(L_y)$:

$$
\bigl[\, L_x \otimes I,\ I \otimes L_y \,\bigr]\varphi
\;=\; (L_x \otimes I)(I \otimes L_y)\varphi \;-\; (I \otimes L_y)(L_x \otimes I)\varphi
\;=\; (L_x \otimes L_y)\varphi \;-\; (L_x \otimes L_y)\varphi
\;=\; 0.
\qquad (10.3)
$$

**Step 2 — exact factorisation of $e^{\tau L}$.** Since $[L_x \otimes I,\,I \otimes L_y] = 0$
on the (dense) tensor-product core, the Trotter–Lie product formula degenerates
to the closed-form factorisation

$$
e^{\tau L} \;=\; e^{\tau (L_x \otimes I)} \cdot e^{\tau (I \otimes L_y)}
\;=\; \widetilde{e^{\tau L_x}} \cdot \widetilde{e^{\tau L_y}},
\qquad (10.4)
$$

valid for all $\tau \ge 0$ (HLW §III.5, Theorem 4.1, special case
$[A,B] = 0$). Each factor is itself a tensor-lift of a 1D semigroup.

**Step 3 — palindromic Strang collapses on commuting flows.** With $A := \widetilde{e^{\tau L_x}}$
and $B := \widetilde{e^{\tau L_y}}$ the *exact* commuting tensor-lifts,
the palindromic Strang formula (10.1) applied to the *exact* 1D flows is

$$
A^{1/2} \cdot B \cdot A^{1/2} \;=\; A \cdot B \;=\; e^{\tau L},
$$

since $A^{1/2}$ and $B$ commute (both diagonal in tensor structure).
This identity is *exact* on the core — palindromic Strang is **bit-equal**
to the true semigroup when applied to commuting flows, with **no
commutator cancellation needed**. (Contrast with §9.4: in 1D operator
splitting $L = A + B$ on a *single* axis, $[A, B] \neq 0$ generically
and Strang's order-2 comes from BCH cancellation of the leading $\tau^3$
commutator.)

**Step 4 — replace exact 1D flows with 1D Chernoff approximants.** By
(H2), each 1D approximant satisfies

$$
\Phi_x(\tau/2) \;=\; e^{(\tau/2) L_x} + O(\tau^3) \quad\text{(local)},
\qquad
\Phi_y(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau L_y} + O(\tau^3) \quad\text{(local)},
$$

on the 1D cores. Lifting to 2D preserves these bounds in sup-norm (a 1D
local error $O(\tau^3)$ measured in $\|\cdot\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb{R}_x)}$
extends to $O(\tau^3)$ in $\|\cdot\|_{L^\infty(\mathbb{R}^2)}$ uniformly
in the frozen axis variable, by the definition of axis-lift). Combined
with (10.4) and the palindromic identity of Step 3:

$$
\Phi^{2D}(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau L} \;+\; O(\tau^3) \quad\text{(per step, sup-norm)}.
\qquad (10.5)
$$

**Step 5 — global lift (Chernoff-product theorem on $L^\infty$).** By
quasi-contractivity (H3) the iterated approximant satisfies

$$
\bigl\| (\Phi^{2D}(\tau))^n - e^{nt L} \bigr\|_\infty
\;\le\; n \cdot O(\tau^3) \cdot e^{T(\omega_x + \omega_y)}
\;=\; T \cdot O(\tau^2) \cdot e^{T(\omega_x + \omega_y)},
$$

i.e. global error $O(\tau^2)$ at fixed $T$. ∎

**Remark 10.1 (no commutator-cancellation budget).** Theorem 7 does *not*
rely on Strang's commutator cancellation in the BCH expansion of
$e^{\tau A} e^{\tau B}$ — that is the §9.4 mechanism for 1D non-commuting
splittings. Here the order-2 lift is **purely a per-axis inheritance**:
each 1D approximant contributes its own per-step $O(\tau^3)$ local error,
and palindromic Strang along axes is exact on commuting flows. **A
consequence**: the regime restrictions of `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A) and
`TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` (TruncatedExp K=4 envelope, ADR-0011) carry over
**per axis** without amplification — the 2D global error is bounded by
the *sum* of per-axis 1D global errors, not their product.

### 10.4 Reduction lemma (the strongest test oracle)

**Lemma 10.2 (Y-independent reduction).** *For any 1D Chernoff functions*
*$\Phi_x, \Phi_y$ as in Theorem 7, and any $f(x, y) = g(x)$ independent*
*of $y$ (i.e., constant in the $y$-direction):*

$$
\Phi^{2D}(\tau, f)(x, y) \;=\; (\Phi_x(\tau) g)(x) \quad\text{for all } y.
\qquad (10.6)
$$

**Proof.** Apply $\widetilde{\Phi}_x(\tau/2)$ first: since $f$ is
$y$-independent, the result is $(\Phi_x(\tau/2) g)(x)$, also
$y$-independent. Apply $\widetilde{\Phi}_y(\tau)$: the input is constant
in $y$, so $\Phi_y(\tau)\bigl(g_x(\cdot)\bigr)$ where $g_x(\cdot)$ is the
constant function $y \mapsto (\Phi_x(\tau/2) g)(x)$. Constants are in the
domain of every quasi-contractive 1D semigroup, and $L_y$ annihilates
constants, so $e^{\tau L_y}\,c = c$ for any constant $c$; by Theorem 6
this equals $\Phi_y(\tau)\,c = c + O(\tau^2)$, exact at $\tau = 0$. **In
the discrete realisation** (`AxisLift<C, Y>::apply` on a Y-independent
input), the floating-point result equals the input pointwise modulo IEEE
rearrangement — at most a few ULPs/node, since `Vec<f64>` cell values are
identical along Y-columns and the 1D `apply` is deterministic per cell.
Apply $\widetilde{\Phi}_x(\tau/2)$ again: input is
$(\Phi_x(\tau/2) g)(x)$, output is $(\Phi_x(\tau)g)(x)$ by the 1D
semigroup law on $\Phi_x(\tau/2)\Phi_x(\tau/2) = \Phi_x(\tau)$ holding
*exactly* (palindromic structure with self-composition is the 1D
identity). **Net**: the Y-pass acts as **identity within FP rounding**
on Y-independent input, and the X-passes self-compose to a single
$\Phi_x(\tau)$ application on $g$. ∎

**Why this is the strongest oracle.** Lemma 10.2 reduces the 2D global
error to the *exact same* 1D global error on $g$ — bit-equal modulo
finite-precision rearrangement. A v0.5.0 acceptance gate that constructs
$f(x, y) = g(x)$ for any v0.3.0+ 1D oracle (heat kernel, advection-
diffusion, Liouville) and runs `Strang2D` on it MUST agree with the
matching 1D run to within ≤16 ULP/node sup-norm — capturing **all** of:
(i) row-major index correctness, (ii) AxisLift adapter correctness,
(iii) 1D `apply` reuse without state corruption.

### 10.5 Order-2 oracles

Two normative 2D oracles for slope verification (G3-strang-2D analogues):

**(a) 2D Gaussian heat kernel** (constant diffusion $a_x = a_y = 1/2$,
$b = c = 0$ on each axis): closed form

$$
u(t, x, y) \;=\; \frac{1}{1 + 2t}\,
\exp\!\Bigl( -\,\frac{x^2 + y^2}{1 + 2t} \Bigr),
\qquad
u(0, x, y) \;=\; e^{-(x^2 + y^2)}.
\qquad (10.7)
$$

This is the tensor product of the v0.1.0 1D heat-kernel oracle (§4) on
each axis. By Lemma 10.2 applied symmetrically (input = $g(x) \cdot
h(y)$ tensor-product, axes commute by separability), the 2D error
**factors** as the product of 1D errors plus a cross-term bounded by
the same envelope.

**(b) Separable advection-diffusion** (Galilean shifted Gaussian on each
axis, $\alpha_x = \beta_x = \alpha_y = \beta_y = 1/2$):

$$
u(t, x, y) \;=\; \frac{1}{1 + 2t}\,
\exp\!\Bigl(
-\,\frac{(x + t/2)^2 + (y + t/2)^2}{1 + 2t}
\Bigr).
\qquad (10.8)
$$

This is the tensor product of the v0.2.0 advection-diffusion oracle
(§9.5) on each axis. Slope $\le -1.95$ on $n \in \{32, 64, 128, 256, 512\}$
verifies the Theorem 7 conclusion empirically (G3-strang-2D gate).

### 10.6 Cross-references

- §1 (Theorem 6) — per-axis Chernoff hypotheses.
- §9.4 — 1D Strang composition (used as a black box per axis).
- §9.5, §9.6 — 1D oracles whose tensor products give the 2D oracles.
- §9.2.3.B (line 1463-1464) — the forward-reference to "$\Phi^{2D}$
  inherits the same per-axis order-2 result" is **anchored here**.
- ADR-0012 — the architectural decision record for v0.5.0.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.tensor.yaml` — Phase 1 struct schema.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` — three new tensor properties
  (`grid_fn_2d_axpy_separability`, `axis_lift_1d_consistency`,
  `strang2d_separable_order_2`).

### 10.7 Out of scope (deferred to v0.7+)

- **Non-separable 2D operators** with cross-derivatives $\partial_x \partial_y$
  (i.e. $[L_x \otimes I, I \otimes L_y] \neq 0$): require genuine 2D
  5-point Chernoff stencils, BCH commutator residual analysis, and a
  separate ADR. Theorem 7 does **not** apply.
- **3D and higher**: the same construction extends inductively but is
  not part of v0.5.0 scope.
- **AMR / FFT / non-uniform grids on 2D**: out of scope per ADR-0012.

(v0.6.0 ADR-0013 adoption removed the previously-listed "4th-order
spatial discretisation in 2D" deferral: `Strang2D::order()` now caps at
4, and `AxisLift<Diffusion4thChernoff>` /
`AxisLift<TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff>` instantiate without changes to
the `axis.rs` body. The 4th-order spatial benefit applies per axis
inheritance, with the constant-`a` regime delivering the headline
$O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$ floor that motivates the v0.6.0 G3⁴-2D slope gate
$\le -3.80$.)

(v0.7.0 ADR-0016 lifts the **non-separable 2D operator** deferral —
see §10.7-bis below.)

---

### 10.7-bis Non-separable 2D operators (NORMATIVE for v0.7.0, ADR-0016, Block C)

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.7.0. Adds `NonSeparable2DChernoff<X, Y>` as a
new public type next to `Strang2D<X, Y>`. The two types are siblings: when
the cross-derivative coefficient $c \equiv 0$, the new type is observably
identical to `Strang2D` modulo IEEE rearrangement (§10.7-bis.6, gate
T7N_zero-c). The §10.7 deferral "non-separable 2D operators" is hereby
**partially lifted**: the scalar mixed-term shape $L = L_x \otimes I + I
\otimes L_y + c(x,y)\,\partial_x \partial_y$ (Option γ in the v0.7.0
plan) is in scope; full anisotropic tensors $\beta(x,y) \cdot
\partial_x \partial_y$ and 4th-cross-derivative leg paths remain
deferred to v0.8+.

#### 10.7-bis.1 Setting

Let $\Omega \subset \mathbb{R}^2$ be a smooth bounded tensor-product
domain (the Cartesian product of two `Grid1D` instances per ADR-0012).
Define the **non-separable 2D generator**

$$
L \;=\; \underbrace{L_x \otimes I}_{=:\,A}
      + \underbrace{I \otimes L_y}_{=:\,B}
      + \underbrace{c(x,y)\,\partial_x \partial_y}_{=:\,M},
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}1)
$$

where:

- **Per-axis legs** $L_x, L_y$ are arbitrary
  `ChernoffFunction<S = GridFn1D>` instances of the v0.5.0+ catalogue
  (`DiffusionChernoff`, `Diffusion4thChernoff`, `Diffusion6thChernoff`,
  `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff`, `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff`).
  Each lifts to a 2D operator via `AxisLift` (§10.2) without
  modification.
- **Mixed leg** $M = c(x,y)\,\partial_x \partial_y$ is the
  cross-derivative term that breaks separability.
- **Coefficient** $c \in C^3(\Omega, \mathbb{R})$ with
  $\|c\|_\infty < \infty$ on the grid domain. The smoothness floor
  $C^3$ is **NORMATIVE** — see §10.7-bis.2 for the `[A,[A,M]]` term
  involving up to $\partial_{xx} c$ that drives this requirement.
- **Ellipticity** (when $L$ is interpreted as a parabolic generator with
  per-axis coefficients $a(x)$ and $b(y)$): the diffusion matrix
  $\bigl[\begin{smallmatrix} a(x) & c(x,y)/2 \\ c(x,y)/2 & b(y) \end{smallmatrix}\bigr]$
  must be positive semi-definite, i.e.
  $$
  c^2(x,y) \;\le\; 4\,a(x)\,b(y) \quad\text{everywhere on } \Omega.
  \qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}2)
  $$
  This is a **doc-only** caller invariant for v0.7.0 (no runtime check;
  violation is a domain modelling error analogous to the existing
  $a > 0$ invariant on `DiffusionChernoff`). Strict inequality is
  required for parabolic regularity of $\exp(\tau L)$ itself; the
  splitting analysis below is unaffected by the inequality margin.

#### 10.7-bis.2 BCH composition — palindromic 5-leg Strang

The v0.7.0 NonSeparable2DChernoff scheme is the **5-leg palindromic
Strang split**

$$
S_5(\tau) \;=\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau A / 2}}_{\text{X}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau B / 2}}_{\text{Y}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau M}}_{\text{cross}}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau B / 2}}_{\text{Y}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau A / 2}}_{\text{X}\,\tau/2}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}3)
$$

**Reduction theorem (NORMATIVE)**: because the per-axis lifts act on
disjoint tensor factors, $[A, B] = 0$ identically (Lemma 10.1 + the
algebra of axis-disjoint lifts). The BCH series for two commuting
operators terminates at the linear term, hence

$$
e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2} \;=\; e^{\tau (A + B) / 2},
\qquad
e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2} \;=\; e^{\tau (A + B) / 2}.
$$

Setting $P := A + B$ and $Q := M$, the 5-leg composition collapses
**exactly** (no $\tau$-truncation) to the standard 2-operator Strang
split:

$$
S_5(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau P / 2}\,e^{\tau Q}\,e^{\tau P / 2}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}4)
$$

This is the workhorse of the analysis — the textbook 2-operator Strang
BCH machinery (HLW 2006 §III.5.2) applies verbatim to the pair $(P, Q)$.

**Standard 2-operator Strang BCH** (HLW 2006 §III.5.2, eq. 5.10)
gives, with all even-order $\tau$-terms vanishing by palindromic
symmetry (HLW 2006 §V.2.1 Theorem 2.2):

$$
\log\bigl(e^{\tau P / 2}\,e^{\tau Q}\,e^{\tau P / 2}\bigr)
\;=\;
\tau\,(P + Q)
\;+\;
\tau^3 \cdot \Bigl[
  -\tfrac{1}{24}\,[P, [P, Q]]
  + \tfrac{1}{12}\,[Q, [Q, P]]
\Bigr]
\;+\; O(\tau^5).
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}5)
$$

Substituting $P = A + B$, $Q = M$, and applying the Jacobi identity
plus $[A, B] = 0$:

$$
[P, [P, M]]
\;=\; [A, [A, M]] + 2\,[A, [B, M]] + [B, [B, M]],
$$
$$
[M, [M, P]]
\;=\; [M, [M, A]] + [M, [M, B]],
$$

so the leading residual at $\tau^3$ is the **NORMATIVE Y₃ formula**:

$$
\boxed{\;
Y_3 \;=\;
-\tfrac{1}{24}\Bigl( [A, [A, M]] + 2\,[A, [B, M]] + [B, [B, M]] \Bigr)
