\;+\; \tfrac{1}{12}\Bigl( [M, [M, A]] + [M, [M, B]] \Bigr).
\;}
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}6)
$$

**Local truncation error**:
$\|S_5(\tau) f - e^{\tau L} f\| = O(\tau^3 \cdot \|f\|_W)$
on a Sobolev-3 norm sufficient for $f \in C^3(\Omega)$ —
the smoothness floor on $c$ is what makes $[A, [A, M]]$ a
densely-defined operator (it contains $\partial_{xx} c$).

**Global error** over $[0, T]$ with $N = T/\tau$ steps (Lady-Windermere
fan accumulation, §11.1):
$\|S_5(\tau)^N f - e^{T L} f\| = O(\tau^2)$. **Order 2 — NORMATIVE.**

#### 10.7-bis.3 Truncated Taylor mixed leg $\Phi_M(\tau)$

The implementation does **not** evaluate $e^{\tau M}$ as an exact
exponential of the mixed-derivative operator (which would require
solving a 2D PDE on its own — defeating the purpose of the splitting).
Instead, the mixed leg uses the **K=2 truncated Taylor expansion**:

$$
\Phi_M(\tau) \;:=\; I \;+\; \tau\,M \;+\; \tfrac{\tau^2}{2}\,M^2,
\qquad
M \;=\; c(x,y)\,\partial_x \partial_y.
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}7)
$$

**Local truncation residue of $\Phi_M$ alone**:

$$
e^{\tau M} \;-\; \Phi_M(\tau) \;=\; \tfrac{\tau^3}{6}\,M^3 + O(\tau^4).
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}8)
$$

The **K=2 composite scheme** is

$$
S_5^{K2}(\tau)
\;:=\;
e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,\Phi_M(\tau)\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2}
\;=\; S_5(\tau) \;+\; \Delta S(\tau),
\qquad
\|\Delta S(\tau)\| = O(\tau^3),
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}9)
$$

so the K=2 perturbation matches the BCH residual at $O(\tau^3)$
locally and **preserves global order 2**.

**Why K=2 is mandatory** (NORMATIVE): if $K = 1$ (i.e. $\Phi_M(\tau) =
I + \tau M$), then $e^{\tau M} - (I + \tau M) = \tfrac{\tau^2}{2} M^2
+ O(\tau^3)$ is $O(\tau^2)$, dominating the BCH residual and dropping
the local error to $O(\tau^2)$ — global $O(\tau^1)$, **order 1, NOT
order 2**. Therefore $K \ge 2$ is the minimum; $K = 3$ does not
improve the global order (still $O(\tau^2)$ capped by Strang) but
slightly reduces the leading constant. The v0.7.0 implementation uses
$K = 2$ for cost.

**Why $\tau^4$ palindromic cancellation is broken**: $\Phi_M(\tau)$ is
**not** time-symmetric to higher orders ($\Phi_M(-\tau) \ne
\Phi_M(\tau)^{-1}$), so the palindromic odd-function property of
eq. (10.7-bis.5) — which annihilates all even $\tau$-powers in
$\log(S_5)$ for the **exact** $e^{\tau M}$ leg — is inherited only at
the leading order by $S_5^{K2}$. This is consistent with the order-2
ceiling.

**Spatial discretisation**: the mixed derivative $\partial_x \partial_y$
is discretised via the **4-point centred cross-stencil** at interior
nodes:

$$
(\partial_x \partial_y f)_{i,j}
\;\approx\;
\frac{f_{i+1, j+1} \;-\; f_{i+1, j-1} \;-\; f_{i-1, j+1} \;+\; f_{i-1, j-1}}
     {4\,\mathrm{dx}\,\mathrm{dy}},
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}10)
$$

with leading truncation residue
$\tfrac{1}{6}\,\mathrm{dx}^2 \cdot \partial_{xxx} \partial_y f
+ \tfrac{1}{6}\,\mathrm{dy}^2 \cdot \partial_x \partial_{yyy} f
+ O(\mathrm{dx}^4)$,
i.e. **$O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$ at the discretisation level**.
At boundary cells where any of $i \pm 1$ or $j \pm 1$ is out of range,
the per-axis `BoundaryPolicy` (§3.5) is applied **independently per
axis**: first along the X-axis at the four ghost positions, then along
the Y-axis. This composition agrees with `Reflect` and `ZeroExtend` on
$C^2$-regular extensions; under `LinearExtrapolate` the second-axis
extension is exact for affine ghost data.

The $M^2$ term in $\Phi_M$ requires applying the 4-point cross-stencil
**twice** (compose two cross-stencils to obtain
$c \cdot \partial_x \partial_y \bigl(c \cdot \partial_x \partial_y f\bigr)$),
which on a uniform grid corresponds to a 9-point support inside a
$\pm 2$ cell box around $(i, j)$.

#### 10.7-bis.4 CFL stability bound

The polynomial $\Phi_M(\tau) = I + \tau M + \tfrac{\tau^2}{2} M^2$ is
**not a contraction** in operator norm — for sufficiently large
$\tau \cdot \|c\|_\infty / (\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy})$ the
$\tau^2 M^2 / 2$ term overwhelms the bounded part. With
$\|\partial_x \partial_y\|_{\text{4pt}} \le 1/(\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy})$
on the centred cross-stencil (Fourier symbol bound at
$k_x = k_y = \pi/2$) and $\|M\|_\infty \le \|c\|_\infty /
(\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy})$, stability of $\Phi_M$ requires

$$
\tau \cdot \|c\|_\infty / (\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}) \;\le\; \theta
\qquad\text{for some } \theta \in (0, 1).
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}11)
$$

The v0.7.0 NORMATIVE choice is **$\theta = 1/4$**, giving the runtime
**CFL gate**

$$
\boxed{\quad 4 \cdot \tau \cdot \|c\|_\infty \;<\; \mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}. \quad}
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}12)
$$

Rationale for $\theta = 1/4$ (vs the analytic limit $\theta < 1/2$):
2× safety margin matches the v0.4.0 `TruncatedExpDiffusionChernoff` CFL
choice (`2·tau·a < dx²` — see §9.2.3.C.CFL). Violation is reported as
**`SemiflowError::CflViolated`** (the existing variant from
ADR-0011 — **no new error variants**); the rustdoc on
`SemiflowError::CflViolated` is amended to document that for
`NonSeparable2DChernoff` the `dx_squared` field semantically holds
the product $\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}$ and `a_norm_bound`
holds $\|c\|_\infty$ (the field names are kept stable for
non-breaking-change reasons; the documentation makes the semantic
overload explicit).

Caller pattern: retry with
$\tau_{\text{safe}} = 0.225 \cdot \mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy} / \|c\|_\infty$
(10% margin below the $\theta = 1/4$ ceiling).

#### 10.7-bis.5 Order claim and oracle

**Type-level invariant** (NORMATIVE): the v0.7.0 `NonSeparable2DChernoff`
implements `ChernoffFunction<S = GridFn2D>` with

$$
\text{order}() \;=\; 2
\qquad\text{(τ-axis Chernoff consistency, per §11.1.bis)}.
$$

The spatial slope at fixed $\tau$ is
$O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$ (cross-stencil eq. 10.7-bis.10) when
the per-axis legs $L_x, L_y$ are themselves $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$
discretisations (e.g. `DiffusionChernoff` ζ-A); higher-order per-axis
legs (`Diffusion4thChernoff`, `Diffusion6thChernoff`) retain their
spatial accuracy on the X- and Y-axis halves but are gated by the
**cross-stencil floor** $O(\mathrm{dx}^2 \cdot \mathrm{dy}^2)$ globally.
Spatial accuracy is **not** advertised by `order()` per §11.1.bis;
spatial slope is observable only via the convergence-slope gate
**G3_NS2D** (§10.7-bis.7).

**Closed-form oracle (rotated 2D Gaussian)**: for the constant-coefficient
PDE
$\partial_t u = a_{xx}\,\partial_{xx} u + a_{yy}\,\partial_{yy} u +
c\,\partial_{xy} u$ with constants $a_{xx}, a_{yy}, c \in \mathbb{R}$
satisfying $c^2 \le 4\,a_{xx}\,a_{yy}$, the exact solution is the
**rotated Gaussian semigroup**:

$$
u(t, x, y)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\det \Sigma_t}}\,
\exp\!\Bigl( -\tfrac{1}{2}\,\xi^\top\,\Sigma_t^{-1}\,\xi \Bigr),
\qquad
\xi = (x, y)^\top,
\qquad
\Sigma_t \;=\; \Sigma_0 + 2\,t\,D,
\qquad
D = \begin{pmatrix} a_{xx} & c/2 \\ c/2 & a_{yy} \end{pmatrix}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-bis.}13)
$$

For the v0.7.0 G3_NS2D test: $\Sigma_0 = I$ (initial datum $u_0 =
e^{-(x^2 + y^2)} / 1$), $a_{xx} = a_{yy} = 0.1$, $c = 0.05$ (well
within ellipticity $0.05^2 = 0.0025 \le 4 \cdot 0.1 \cdot 0.1 = 0.04$),
giving
$\Sigma_t = \bigl[\begin{smallmatrix} 1 + 0.2\,t & 0.05\,t \\ 0.05\,t & 1 + 0.2\,t \end{smallmatrix}\bigr]$
and the explicit closed form
$u(t, x, y) = (\det \Sigma_t)^{-1/2} \exp(-\tfrac{1}{2}\,\xi^\top \Sigma_t^{-1}\,\xi)$.

**Verification that eq. (10.7-bis.13) solves the PDE**: direct
substitution gives
$\partial_t u = -\tfrac{1}{2}\,\mathrm{tr}(\Sigma_t^{-1}\,\partial_t \Sigma_t)\,u
+ \tfrac{1}{2}\,\xi^\top\,\Sigma_t^{-1}\,(\partial_t \Sigma_t)\,\Sigma_t^{-1}\,\xi\,u$
and $\partial_t \Sigma_t = 2 D$. Computing
$a_{xx}\,\partial_{xx} u + a_{yy}\,\partial_{yy} u + c\,\partial_{xy} u$
on the rotated Gaussian yields the matching expression after
recognising $(\Sigma_t^{-1})\,D\,(\Sigma_t^{-1}) =
\partial_t (\Sigma_t^{-1}) / (-2)$ and
$\mathrm{tr}(\Sigma_t^{-1}\,D) = \mathrm{tr}(D\,\Sigma_t^{-1})$. The
architect's sympy script `verify_v0_7_0_nonseparable.py` gate
**T7N_oracle** verifies this symbolically.

#### 10.7-bis.6 NORMATIVE sympy gates

Mirroring the v0.6.0 / v0.7.0 ζ⁴ / ζ⁶ gate pattern (§9.2.4 / §9.2.6),
the architect's verification script
`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_7_0_nonseparable.py` MUST
exit 0 with all the following gates passing:

| Gate | Statement |
|------|-----------|
| **T7N_τ²** | $\log(S_5(\tau))\bigm|_{\tau^2} = 0$ for the exact-$e^{\tau M}$ leg (palindromic cancellation, eq. 10.7-bis.5 with $P = A + B$, $Q = M$, $[A, B] = 0$). |
| **T7N_τ³** | $\log(S_5(\tau))\bigm|_{\tau^3} = Y_3$ exactly, with $Y_3$ as in eq. (10.7-bis.6). Verified after canonicalising the $[A, B] = 0$ algebra (Appendix). |
| **T7N_K2_local** | $S_5^{K2}(\tau) - e^{\tau L}$ has no $\tau^k$ terms for $k \in \{0, 1, 2\}$ and a non-zero $\tau^3$ leading term. Confirms K=2 truncation preserves local order 3 / global order 2. |
| **T7N_oracle** | The rotated Gaussian $u(t, x, y)$ of eq. (10.7-bis.13) satisfies $\partial_t u = a_{xx}\,\partial_{xx} u + a_{yy}\,\partial_{yy} u + c\,\partial_{xy} u$ identically. |
| **T7N_zero-c** | Setting $c \equiv 0$ in eq. (10.7-bis.7), the K=2 mixed leg degenerates to $\Phi_M(\tau) = I$ exactly; hence $S_5^{K2}(\tau)\bigm|_{c \equiv 0}$ is symbolically identical to the pure 5-leg axis composition $e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2} = e^{\tau (A + B)/2}\,e^{\tau (A + B)/2} = e^{\tau (A + B)}$, which (by Lemma 10.1 with $[A, B] = 0$) is the same operator as the 3-leg `Strang2D` symbolically. The implementation MUST detect $c \equiv 0$ at construction time and branch to the 3-leg `Strang2D` apply (no $\Phi_M$ multiplication by $I$) so the FP result is bit-equal to the existing `Strang2D` path on the same per-axis legs. |
| **T7N_palindrome** | The leg sequence $[A/2, B/2, M, B/2, A/2]$ equals its own reverse — static gate protecting against future refactor-induced reordering. |

**Canonicalisation gotcha** (NORMATIVE for the script): sympy's default
`expr.replace(A*B, B*A)` does **not** recurse into noncommutative
substrings inside longer monomials (e.g. `C*A*B*D` is not matched). The
script MUST adopt the custom recursive `canonicalize_AB(expr)` helper
that walks the operator tree and rewrites consecutive $A\,B \to B\,A$
substrings to fixed-point. See the script's Appendix and the
researcher analysis `.dev-docs/research/non-separable-2d-bch.md` §6.

#### 10.7-bis.7 G3_NS2D slope gate (NORMATIVE)

The v0.7.0 release-headline gate for `NonSeparable2DChernoff` is the
**G3_NS2D 1D-equivalent slope test**:

| Parameter | Value |
|-----------|-------|
| Domain | $[-5, 5]^2$ |
| Final time $T$ | $0.5$ |
| Time steps $n$ | $200$ (fixed) |
| Per-axis grid sizes $N$ | $\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ |
| Per-axis diffusion $a_{xx}, a_{yy}$ | $0.1$ (constant) |
| Cross-coefficient $c$ | $0.05$ (constant) — well inside ellipticity $c^2 = 0.0025 \le 4 a_{xx} a_{yy} = 0.04$ |
| Inner per-axis legs | `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A) on each axis |
| Initial datum | $u_0(x, y) = e^{-(x^2 + y^2)}$ |
| Oracle | Rotated Gaussian eq. (10.7-bis.13) at $t = T = 0.5$ |
| Slope (OLS over $\log_2$-error vs $\log_2 N$) | $\le -1.95$ |

The gate threshold $-1.95$ matches the v0.5.0 G3-2D constant
($-1.95$ on `Strang2D<DiffusionChernoff, DiffusionChernoff>`), with
expected achieved slope $\approx -2.0 \pm 0.05$ (analogous to the
v0.5.0 G3-2D measurement at $-2.056$). The 0.05 buffer below the claim
is identical to G3-2D's buffer ratio.

A **secondary variant** with variable $c(x, y) = 0.05 \cdot
\tanh(x + y)$ (smooth, bounded by $0.05$, $C^\infty$) is gated under
**G3_NS2D_var** at the same threshold $-1.95$. This exercises the
$[A, [B, M]]$ commutator in $Y_3$ which vanishes for constant $c$
(making G3_NS2D itself a partial test of the BCH analysis).

**Cross-references**:
- §10.7 — original deferral note (now partially lifted by ADR-0016).
- §11.1.bis — axis distinction NORMATIVE clarification (τ-axis $p = 2$,
  spatial dx-axis observed via slope gate only).
- ADR-0012 — `Strang2D` predecessor type that `NonSeparable2DChernoff`
  observably degenerates to when $c \equiv 0$.
- ADR-0011 — `SemiflowError::CflViolated` variant, reused with semantic
  field overload (rustdoc amendment only).
- ADR-0016 — the v0.7.0 architectural decision record.
- `.dev-docs/research/non-separable-2d-bch.md` — researcher analysis
  with full BCH derivation, sympy reproduction recipe, and the
  canonicalisation Appendix.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.tensor.yaml` — Phase 1 struct schema (to be
  amended by Engineer with `NonSeparable2DChernoff` schema).
- `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` — three new properties
  (T7N_*, G3_NS2D, G3_NS2D_var) to be added with `severity: NORMATIVE`.

### 10.7-ter Anisotropic 2D non-separable operators (NORMATIVE for v0.9.0, ADR-0023, Block A)

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.9.0. Adds
`NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff<X, Y>` as an additive sibling of the
v0.7.0 `NonSeparable2DChernoff<X, Y>` — the two are siblings, not
replacements: when the anisotropic mixed-term coefficient
$\beta \equiv 0$, the new type is observably identical to `Strang2D`
modulo IEEE rearrangement (§10.7-ter.6, gate T9N_zero-β); when $\beta$
is the constant scalar $c$, the new type is symbolically identical to
`NonSeparable2DChernoff` modulo the documented field-name and CFL-form
adjustment. The §10.7 / §10.7-bis "anisotropic full-tensor
$\beta(x, y) \cdot \partial_x \partial_y$" deferral (§10.7-bis preamble
lines 3119–3121, ADR-0016 forward-compat lines 156–161) is hereby
**lifted** for the additive-sibling shape; full off-diagonal $2 \times 2$
diffusion-tensor matrices $D(x, y)$ breaking per-axis product structure
remain out of scope (a future `Coupled2DChernoff` is a different
architecture — see ADR-0023 alternatives §(e)). 4th-cross-derivative
legs $\partial_x^3 \partial_y$ and $\partial_x \partial_y^3$ remain
deferred to a future ADR.

#### 10.7-ter.1 Setting

Let $\Omega \subset \mathbb{R}^2$ be a smooth bounded tensor-product
domain (§10.7-bis.1). Define the **anisotropic non-separable 2D
generator**

$$
L \;=\; \underbrace{L_x \otimes I}_{=:\,A}
      + \underbrace{I \otimes L_y}_{=:\,B}
      + \underbrace{\beta(x,y)\,\partial_x \partial_y}_{=:\,M_\beta},
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}1)
$$

where the **per-axis legs** $A, B$ and **mixed leg** $M_\beta$ have the
following invariants:

- **Per-axis legs $A, B$**: identical to §10.7-bis.1 — arbitrary
  v0.5.0+ catalogue `ChernoffFunction<S = GridFn1D>` instances lifted
  via `AxisLift` (§10.2). **No change** from v0.7.0 — this is the
  central observation that makes the full §10.7-bis BCH analysis
  inheritable. See §10.7-bis.1 for the full catalogue (no duplication
  here).
- **Mixed leg** $M_\beta = \beta(x, y) \cdot \partial_x \partial_y$ is
  the anisotropic position-dependent cross-derivative term, with
  $\beta \in C^3(\Omega, \mathbb{R})$ (NORMATIVE — needed so
  $[A, [A, M_\beta]]$ containing $\partial_{xx} \beta$ is densely
  defined; identical regularity floor to v0.7.0 with $c \to \beta$
  relabel) and $\|\beta\|_\infty < \infty$ on the grid domain.
- **Ellipticity** (when $L_x, L_y$ are second-order parabolic with
  per-axis coefficients $a(x)$ and $b(y)$): the diffusion matrix
  $\bigl[\begin{smallmatrix} a(x) & \beta(x,y)/2 \\ \beta(x,y)/2 & b(y) \end{smallmatrix}\bigr]$
  must be positive semi-definite, i.e.
  $$
  \beta^2(x, y) \;\le\; 4\,a(x)\,b(y) \quad\text{everywhere on } \Omega.
  \qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}2)
  $$
  This is a **doc-only** caller invariant (no runtime check; analogous
  to eq. 10.7-bis.2 with the substitution $c \to \beta$). Strict
  inequality is required for parabolic regularity of $\exp(\tau L)$;
  the splitting analysis below is unaffected by the inequality margin.

#### 10.7-ter.2 BCH composition — palindromic 5-leg Strang

The v0.9.0 `NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff` scheme is the **5-leg
palindromic Strang split** with $M_\beta$ in place of $M$:

$$
S_5(\tau) \;=\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau A / 2}}_{\text{X}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau B / 2}}_{\text{Y}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau M_\beta}}_{\text{cross-aniso}}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau B / 2}}_{\text{Y}\,\tau/2}\;\cdot\;
\underbrace{e^{\tau A / 2}}_{\text{X}\,\tau/2}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}3)
$$

**Reduction theorem (NORMATIVE — inherited verbatim from §10.7-bis.2)**:
because the per-axis legs $A, B$ are **unchanged** from v0.7.0
(axis-disjoint tensor lifts via `AxisLift`), the commutator identity
$[A, B] = 0$ (Lemma 10.1) is preserved. The §10.7-bis.2 proof of the
5-leg → 2-operator collapse depends **only** on $[A, B] = 0$ — nowhere
does it use any property of the mixed leg beyond its identity as a
single operator. Hence the proof carries over to $M_\beta$ verbatim:
setting $P := A + B$ and $Q := M_\beta$, the 5-leg composition collapses
**exactly** (no $\tau$-truncation) to the standard 2-operator Strang
split

$$
S_5(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau P / 2}\,e^{\tau Q}\,e^{\tau P / 2}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}4)
$$

The textbook 2-operator Strang BCH machinery (HLW 2006 §III.5.2) and
the palindromic odd-function logarithm (HLW 2006 §V.2.1 Theorem 2.2)
both apply verbatim to $(P, Q) = (A + B, M_\beta)$, giving (eq.
10.7-bis.5 with $Q \to M_\beta$):

$$
\log\bigl(e^{\tau P / 2}\,e^{\tau Q}\,e^{\tau P / 2}\bigr)
\;=\;
\tau\,(P + Q)
\;+\;
\tau^3 \cdot \Bigl[
  -\tfrac{1}{24}\,[P, [P, Q]]
  + \tfrac{1}{12}\,[Q, [Q, P]]
\Bigr]
\;+\; O(\tau^5).
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}5)
$$

Substituting $P = A + B$, $Q = M_\beta$, and applying $[A, B] = 0$
exactly as in §10.7-bis.2 yields the **NORMATIVE Y₃ formula** for the
anisotropic case:

$$
\boxed{\;
Y_3 \;=\;
-\tfrac{1}{24}\Bigl( [A, [A, M_\beta]] + 2\,[A, [B, M_\beta]] + [B, [B, M_\beta]] \Bigr)
\;+\; \tfrac{1}{12}\Bigl( [M_\beta, [M_\beta, A]] + [M_\beta, [M_\beta, B]] \Bigr).
\;}
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}6)
$$

The structure is **identical** to eq. (10.7-bis.6) under the relabel
$M \to M_\beta$ — sympy gate **T9N_τ³** verifies this symbolically by
substituting $M \to M_\beta$ at the noncommutative-symbol level (see
§10.7-ter.6 below).

**Local truncation error**:
$\|S_5(\tau) f - e^{\tau L} f\| = O(\tau^3 \cdot \|f\|_W)$ on a
Sobolev-3 norm sufficient for $f \in C^3(\Omega)$ — the smoothness floor
on $\beta$ makes $[A, [A, M_\beta]]$ a densely-defined operator
(it contains $\partial_{xx} \beta$).

**Global error** over $[0, T]$ with $N = T / \tau$ steps (Lady-Windermere
fan accumulation, §11.1):
$\|S_5(\tau)^N f - e^{T L} f\| = O(\tau^2)$. **Order 2 — NORMATIVE.**

#### 10.7-ter.3 Truncated Taylor mixed leg $\Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau)$

As in v0.7.0, the implementation does **not** evaluate $e^{\tau M_\beta}$
as an exact exponential of the mixed-derivative operator (which would
require solving a 2D PDE on its own). The mixed leg uses the **K=2
truncated Taylor expansion**:

$$
\Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau) \;:=\; I \;+\; \tau\,M_\beta \;+\; \tfrac{\tau^2}{2}\,M_\beta^2,
\qquad
M_\beta \;=\; \beta(x, y)\,\partial_x \partial_y.
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}7)
$$

**Local truncation residue of $\Phi_{M_\beta}$ alone**:

$$
e^{\tau M_\beta} \;-\; \Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau) \;=\; \tfrac{\tau^3}{6}\,M_\beta^3 + O(\tau^4).
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}8)
$$

The **K=2 composite scheme** is

$$
S_5^{K2}(\tau)
\;:=\;
e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,\Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau)\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2}
\;=\; S_5(\tau) \;+\; \Delta S(\tau),
\qquad
\|\Delta S(\tau)\| = O(\tau^3),
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}9)
$$

so the K=2 perturbation matches the BCH residual at $O(\tau^3)$ locally
and **preserves global order 2**.

**Why K=2 is mandatory** (NORMATIVE): the §10.7-bis.3 K=1 counterexample
applies verbatim to $M_\beta$. With $K = 1$, $e^{\tau M_\beta} - (I + \tau
M_\beta) = \tfrac{\tau^2}{2} M_\beta^2 + O(\tau^3)$ is $O(\tau^2)$,
dominating the BCH residual and dropping local error to $O(\tau^2)$ →
global $O(\tau^1)$. The proof depends only on the leading $\tau^2 M^2 / 2$
term being non-zero, which holds for $M_\beta$ identically. K=3 does
not improve the global order (still capped by Strang); the v0.9.0
implementation uses K=2 for cost.

**Spatial discretisation**: the mixed derivative $\partial_x \partial_y$
uses the same **4-point centred cross-stencil** as v0.7.0 (eq. 10.7-bis.10)
at interior nodes, multiplied **pointwise** by $\beta(x_i, y_j)$:

$$
(M_\beta f)_{i,j}
\;\approx\;
\beta(x_i, y_j) \cdot
\frac{f_{i+1, j+1} \;-\; f_{i+1, j-1} \;-\; f_{i-1, j+1} \;+\; f_{i-1, j-1}}
     {4\,\mathrm{dx}\,\mathrm{dy}},
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}10)
$$

with leading truncation residue
$\beta(x, y) \cdot \bigl[\tfrac{1}{6}\,\mathrm{dx}^2 \cdot \partial_{xxx} \partial_y f
+ \tfrac{1}{6}\,\mathrm{dy}^2 \cdot \partial_x \partial_{yyy} f\bigr]
+ O(\mathrm{dx}^4 + \mathrm{dy}^4)$,
i.e. **$O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$ at the discretisation level** —
the pointwise $\beta(x, y)$ factor is bounded by $\|\beta\|_\infty$ and
does not affect the spatial order.

**Stencil shape unchanged from v0.7.0 — no boundary-policy work**: the
4 neighbour positions $(i \pm 1, j \pm 1)$ are identical to
eq. (10.7-bis.10); only the scalar pointwise multiplier per node
changes. The §10.7-bis.3 boundary-policy composition rules
(`Reflect` and `ZeroExtend` on $C^2$-regular extensions; exact for
affine ghost data under `LinearExtrapolate`) carry over without any
new boundary-policy work.

The $M_\beta^2$ term in $\Phi_{M_\beta}$ requires applying the
$\beta$-weighted cross-stencil **twice** — composing two
$\beta$-weighted stencils gives the inner-ring product
$\beta(x_i, y_j) \cdot \beta(x_k, y_l)$ at the 5×5 effective box
support per node (the $\pm 2$ cells reachable by two stencil steps).
The stencil-shape signature is identical to v0.7.0 (the $M^2$ box
support); only the scalar weighting at each node changes.

#### 10.7-ter.4 CFL stability bound

The polynomial $\Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau) = I + \tau M_\beta +
\tfrac{\tau^2}{2} M_\beta^2$ is not a contraction in operator norm —
the analysis is identical to §10.7-bis.4 with $c \to \beta$.
With the centred cross-stencil Fourier-symbol bound
$\|\partial_x \partial_y\|_{\text{4pt}} \le 1 / (\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy})$
and the pointwise $\beta$ multiplier giving

$$
\|M_\beta\|_\infty \;\le\; \|\beta\|_\infty / (\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}),
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}11)
$$

stability of $\Phi_{M_\beta}$ requires $\tau \cdot \|\beta\|_\infty /
(\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}) \le \theta$ for some $\theta \in (0, 1)$.
The v0.9.0 NORMATIVE choice is **$\theta = 1/4$** (preserving the
v0.7.0 / v0.4.0 2× safety margin; see §9.2.3.C.CFL and §10.7-bis.4 for
rationale), giving the runtime **CFL gate**:

$$
\boxed{\quad 4 \cdot \tau \cdot \|\beta\|_\infty \;<\; \mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}. \quad}
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}12)
$$

Note the convention: the violation field carries the product
$\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}$ (NOT $\mathrm{dx}^2$), identical to the
v0.7.0 §10.7-bis.4 convention. Violation is reported as
**`SemiflowError::CflViolated`** (the existing variant from ADR-0011 —
no new error variants); the rustdoc on `SemiflowError::CflViolated` is
amended in Block B to document the third semantic field overload
(`a_norm_bound` semantically holds $\|\beta\|_\infty$ for
`NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff`, in addition to the existing
$\|a\|_\infty$ from v0.4.0 and $\|c\|_\infty$ from v0.7.0). The
`dx_squared` field continues to hold the product
$\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}$ in this context (same as v0.7.0).

Caller pattern: retry with $\tau_{\text{safe}} = 0.225 \cdot \mathrm{dx}
\cdot \mathrm{dy} / \|\beta\|_\infty$ (10% margin below the
$\theta = 1/4$ ceiling).

#### 10.7-ter.5 Order claim and oracle

**Type-level invariant** (NORMATIVE): the v0.9.0
`NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff` implements
`ChernoffFunction<S = GridFn2D>` with

$$
\text{order}() \;=\; 2
\qquad\text{(τ-axis Chernoff consistency, per §11.1.bis)}.
$$

The spatial slope at fixed $\tau$ is $O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$
(cross-stencil eq. 10.7-ter.10) when the per-axis legs $L_x, L_y$ are
themselves $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ discretisations (e.g. `DiffusionChernoff`
ζ-A); higher-order per-axis legs (`Diffusion4thChernoff`,
`Diffusion6thChernoff`) retain their per-axis spatial accuracy on the
X- and Y-axis halves but are **gated by the cross-stencil floor**
$O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$ globally — the same
**Strang-floor cap** documented at §10.7-bis.5. Spatial accuracy is not
advertised by `order()` per §11.1.bis; spatial slope is observable only
via the convergence-slope gate **G4_NS2D_aniso** (§10.7-ter.7).

**Closed-form oracle (rotated 2D Gaussian)**: for the constant-coefficient
PDE
$\partial_t u = a_{xx}\,\partial_{xx} u + a_{yy}\,\partial_{yy} u +
\beta\,\partial_{xy} u$ with constants $a_{xx}, a_{yy}, \beta \in
\mathbb{R}$ satisfying $\beta^2 \le 4\,a_{xx}\,a_{yy}$, the exact
solution is the rotated Gaussian semigroup of eq. (10.7-bis.13) with
$c \to \beta$:

$$
u(t, x, y)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\det \Sigma_t}}\,
\exp\!\Bigl( -\tfrac{1}{2}\,\xi^\top\,\Sigma_t^{-1}\,\xi \Bigr),
\qquad
\xi = (x, y)^\top,
\qquad
\Sigma_t \;=\; \Sigma_0 + 2\,t\,D,
\qquad
D = \begin{pmatrix} a_{xx} & \beta/2 \\ \beta/2 & a_{yy} \end{pmatrix}.
\qquad (10.7\text{-ter.}13)
$$

For the v0.9.0 G4_NS2D_aniso slope test, $\beta$ is now
**position-dependent**: $\beta(x, y) = 0.05 \cdot \exp(-(x^2 + y^2)/4)$
— smooth, $C^\infty$, bounded by $0.05$, and exercising the
$[A, [B, M_\beta]]$ commutator with non-trivial spatial dependence
beyond the constant-$c$ secondary variant of §10.7-bis.7. With the
position-dependent $\beta$ the closed-form oracle eq. (10.7-ter.13)
holds **only locally** (frozen-coefficient sense at each point); the
slope gate compares the numerical solution against the semigroup
generated by the variable-coefficient PDE evolved on a much finer
grid (high-resolution reference solution per the v0.5.0 G3-2D pattern,
§10.5.4). Sympy gate **T9N_oracle** verifies eq. (10.7-ter.13) at the
constant-$\beta$ slice (frozen-coefficient consistency). The
Strang-floor cap on slope ($O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$) applies independently
of constant- vs variable-$\beta$.

#### 10.7-ter.6 NORMATIVE sympy gates

Mirroring the v0.7.0 T7N_* pattern (§10.7-bis.6), the architect's
verification script
`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v0_9_0_nonseparable_aniso.py`
MUST exit 0 with all the following gates passing:

| Gate | Statement |
|------|-----------|
| **T9N_τ²** | $\log(S_5(\tau))\bigm|_{\tau^2} = 0$ for the exact-$e^{\tau M_\beta}$ leg (palindromic cancellation, eq. 10.7-ter.5 with $P = A + B$, $Q = M_\beta$, $[A, B] = 0$). Identical proof to T7N_τ² with $M \to M_\beta$. |
| **T9N_τ³** | $\log(S_5(\tau))\bigm|_{\tau^3} = Y_3$ exactly, with $Y_3$ as in eq. (10.7-ter.6). Verified after canonicalising the $[A, B] = 0$ algebra (Appendix). |
| **T9N_K2_local** | $S_5^{K2}(\tau) - e^{\tau L}$ has no $\tau^k$ terms for $k \in \{0, 1, 2\}$ and a non-zero $\tau^3$ leading term. Confirms K=2 truncation preserves local order 3 / global order 2 in the anisotropic case. |
| **T9N_oracle** | The rotated Gaussian $u(t, x, y)$ of eq. (10.7-ter.13) satisfies the constant-coefficient PDE $\partial_t u = a_{xx}\,\partial_{xx} u + a_{yy}\,\partial_{yy} u + \beta\,\partial_{xy} u$ identically (frozen-coefficient consistency). |
| **T9N_zero-β** | Setting $\beta \equiv 0$ in eq. (10.7-ter.7), the K=2 mixed leg degenerates to $\Phi_{M_\beta}(\tau) = I$ exactly; hence $S_5^{K2}(\tau)\bigm|_{\beta \equiv 0}$ is symbolically identical to the pure 5-leg axis composition $e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2} = e^{\tau (A + B)}$, which (by Lemma 10.1 with $[A, B] = 0$) is the same operator as the 3-leg `Strang2D` symbolically. The implementation MUST detect $\beta \equiv 0$ at construction time (via `beta_norm_bound == 0.0`) and branch to the 3-leg `Strang2D` apply (no $\Phi_{M_\beta}$ multiplication by $I$) so the FP result is bit-equal to the existing `Strang2D` path on the same per-axis legs. |
| **T9N_palindrome** | The leg sequence $[A/2, B/2, M_\beta, B/2, A/2]$ equals its own reverse — static gate protecting against future refactor-induced reordering. |

**Reuse note (NORMATIVE for the script)**: the v0.9.0 verifier reuses
`canonicalize_AB(expr)` from the v0.7.0
`verify_v0_7_0_nonseparable.py` script verbatim. The only change is a
single-symbol relabel at the sympy noncommutative-symbol layer:
introduce `M_beta = sp.Symbol('M_beta', commutative=False)` and
substitute `M -> M_beta` throughout. This is a pure relabel — no
algorithmic change to `canonicalize_AB`, no new BCH derivation, no new
canonicalisation logic. The §10.7-bis.6 canonicalisation gotcha
(`expr.replace(A*B, B*A)` does not recurse into noncommutative
substrings inside longer monomials) applies verbatim and the Appendix
note in the v0.7.0 script suffices.

#### 10.7-ter.7 G4_NS2D_aniso slope gate (NORMATIVE)

The v0.9.0 release-headline gate for `NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff`
is the **G4_NS2D_aniso 1D-equivalent slope test**:

| Parameter | Value |
|-----------|-------|
| Domain | $[-5, 5]^2$ |
| Final time $T$ | $0.5$ |
| Time steps $n$ | $500$ (fixed; CFL-safe at finest grid $511 \times 511$ nodes) |
| Per-axis grid sizes $N$ | $\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ |
| Per-axis diffusion $a_{xx}, a_{yy}$ | $0.1$ (constant) |
| Anisotropic cross-coefficient $\beta(x, y)$ | $0.05 \cdot \exp(-(x^2 + y^2)/4)$ — smooth, $C^\infty$, bounded by $0.05$, non-constant |
| Inner per-axis legs | `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A) on each axis |
| Initial datum | $u_0(x, y) = e^{-(x^2 + y^2)}$ |
| Reference oracle | Self-convergence (mirror v0.7.0 §10.7-bis.7 G3_NS2D_var): for each probe $N$, also compute on the fine $2N{-}1$ grid; coarse error is the sup-norm of (coarse vs downsampled fine). No separate high-resolution reference — eliminates reference-solution-floor at asymptotic $N$. |
| Slope (OLS over $\log_2$-error vs $\log_2 N$) | $\le -1.95$ (unchanged; matches v0.7.0 G3_NS2D_var threshold under Strang-floor inheritance) |
| Pre-asymptotic skip | $N = 32$ excluded from OLS slope (mirror v0.7.0 G3_NS2D_var convention; tanh-like spatial features at coarse $\mathrm{dx}$ are not yet in the $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ regime) |

The self-convergence design replaces the earlier $N_{\text{ref}} = 1024$
reference-grid approach. The $N_{\text{ref}} = 1024$ reference carries
residual error $\approx 10^{-3}$; at $N = 256$ the probe error reaches
that floor, producing non-monotone errors and a collapsed slope
($\approx -0.31$). Self-convergence — comparing each probe $N$ against
its next-finer $2N{-}1$ companion and downsampling the fine solution to
coarse nodes — removes the reference floor entirely so the spatial
$O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ rate is measured without a fixed ceiling. The pattern
is a direct mirror of the proven v0.7.0 G3_NS2D_var secondary variant
(§10.7-bis.7), applied unchanged to the anisotropic $\beta(x, y)$
setting.

**CFL analysis**: $\tau = T/n = 0.5/500 = 10^{-3}$. Finest comparison
grid: $2 \cdot 256 - 1 = 511$ nodes on domain $[-5, 5]$, giving
$\mathrm{dx} = 10/510 \approx 0.01961$ and
$\mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy} \approx 3.84 \times 10^{-4}$. CFL gate:
$4\tau \|\beta\|_\infty = 4 \cdot 10^{-3} \cdot 0.05 = 2.0 \times 10^{-4}
< 3.84 \times 10^{-4}$ — passes with $\approx 1.92\times$ margin at the
finest grid.

**Mechanism note (NORMATIVE, ratified by gate suite)**: the order-2
claim emerges JOINTLY from three components inherited from §10.7-bis:
**(a)** the palindromic 5-leg structure (combined with $[A, B] = 0$,
unchanged from v0.7.0); **(b)** the K=2 truncated Taylor mixed leg,
which matches the BCH residual order $O(\tau^3)$ locally; **(c)** the
$\beta$-weighted 4-point centred cross-stencil for $\partial_x
\partial_y$ at $O(\mathrm{dx}^2 + \mathrm{dy}^2)$ on $C^4$-smooth data
with bounded $\beta$. The non-trivial spatial dependence of $\beta(x, y)
= 0.05 \cdot \exp(-(x^2 + y^2)/4)$ exercises the $[A, [B, M_\beta]]$
commutator (which is non-zero precisely when $\beta$ is not constant
along the relevant axis) — a strictly stronger BCH-coverage test than
the v0.7.0 G3_NS2D constant-$c$ default and a peer of the v0.7.0
G3_NS2D_var $0.05 \cdot \tanh(x + y)$ secondary variant.

**Empirical validation (2026-05-07)**: with the self-convergence design
and the $N$ basket $\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$, the achieved OLS slope (on
$\{64, 128, 256\}$) is $\approx -2.20$, satisfying the $\le -1.95$ gate.
Errors: $\{1.47 \times 10^{-2},\, 4.58 \times 10^{-3},\, 1.11 \times 10^{-3},\, 2.18 \times 10^{-4}\}$ (monotone).
Wallclock: $\approx 7$ minutes on a contemporary workstation with
`RUSTFLAGS="-C target-cpu=native"` and
`--features parallel,simd,slow-tests --release`. The heavy validation is
invoked manually via `cargo run -p xtask -- test-flagship`; the spec is
normative, the empirical run validates the chosen $N$ basket.

**Cross-references**:

- §10.7-bis (parent scalar-$c$ section — shared per-axis-leg machinery,
  §10.7-bis.2 5-leg → 2-operator collapse proof inherited verbatim,
  §10.7-bis.3 K=2 mandate, §10.7-bis.4 CFL-gate shape).
- §10.7 — original deferral note (now further partially lifted by ADR-0023).
- §11.1.bis — axis distinction NORMATIVE clarification (τ-axis $p = 2$,
  spatial dx-axis observable via slope gate only).
- ADR-0023 — the v0.9.0 architectural decision record (this section's
  normative companion).
- ADR-0016 — v0.7.0 scalar-$c$ predecessor (proof inherited verbatim
  with $M \to M_\beta$ substitution; ADR-0023 ratifies the
  forward-compat clause at lines 156–161).
- ADR-0012 — `Strang2D` predecessor type that
  `NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff` observably degenerates to when
  $\beta \equiv 0$ (gate T9N_zero-β codifies the bit-equal degeneration).

---

### 10.8 Tensor product to N axes — 3D specialisation

#### 10.8.1 Setting (3D separable tensor product) and Lemma 10.1

The 3D separable tensor-product setting on $H = H_x \otimes H_y \otimes H_z$:
the generator decomposes as

$$
L \;=\; (L_x \otimes I \otimes I) \;+\; (I \otimes L_y \otimes I) \;+\;
(I \otimes I \otimes L_z),
\qquad (10.8.1)
$$

with each $L_\ast$ a quasi-contractive generator on its respective Hilbert
space (H1–H3 of §1, per axis). Per-axis lifts:

$$
A \;:=\; L_x \otimes I \otimes I, \quad
B \;:=\; I \otimes L_y \otimes I, \quad
C \;:=\; I \otimes I \otimes L_z.
$$

**Lemma 10.1 (axis-disjoint commutation, inductive form).** *For tensor
products $H = \bigotimes_{i=1}^{N} H_i$ and any two operators*
*$T_i := T \otimes I_{j \neq i}$ and $S_j := S \otimes I_{k \neq j}$ acting*
*nontrivially on disjoint tensor factors ($i \neq j$): $[T_i, S_j] = 0$.*

*Proof.* By the universal property of the tensor product, both compositions
factor identically:
$$
T_i \cdot S_j \;=\; (T \otimes I)(I \otimes S) \;=\; T \otimes S \;=\;
(I \otimes S)(T \otimes I) \;=\; S_j \cdot T_i,
$$
modulo the obvious reordering of identity factors on indices $\{1, \ldots,
N\} \setminus \{i, j\}$ (which acts by the trivial reorder of identity
operators). ∎

**Note (retroactive scope).** The N=2 specialisation of Lemma 10.1 is the
implicit lemma cited in §10.7-bis.2 (eq. 10.7-bis.3 → 4 collapse,
line 3180), §10.7-bis.6 gate **T7N_zero-c** (line 3452), §10.7-ter.2
(line 3591), and §10.7-ter.6 gate **T9N_zero-β** (line 3845). All four
prior cite-sites use Lemma 10.1 with semantics "axis-disjoint tensor lifts
commute" — exactly the **N=2 special case** of the inductive lemma stated
above. Hence those cites are well-defined under this lemma without prose
edits at the cite-sites: their existing wording "$[A, B] = 0$ (Lemma 10.1
+ the algebra of axis-disjoint lifts)" is correct and the lemma name now
resolves.

The N=3 specialisation gives **pairwise commutation** of the three per-axis
lifts:

$$
[A, B] \;=\; [A, C] \;=\; [B, C] \;=\; 0.
\qquad (10.8.2)
$$

Domain regularity: $f \in C^3(\Omega_x \times \Omega_y \times \Omega_z)$ for
the per-axis Chernoff Sobolev floors of Theorem 7 (per axis, sup-norm; same
hypothesis as §10.3 lifted by tensor-product trace).

#### 10.8.2 Theorem 7' (inductive, N=3 specialisation)

**Theorem 7' (N-axis Chernoff lift).** *Let $\Phi_i$ ($i = 1, \ldots, N$)
be 1D Chernoff functions satisfying H1–H3 with per-step local error*
*$\Phi_i(\tau) = e^{\tau L_i} + O(\tau^{p_i + 1})$. Define the N-axis
palindromic Strang composition $S_N(\tau)$ on $\bigotimes H_i$ as the*
*nested palindrome*

$$
S_N(\tau) \;=\; \widetilde{\Phi}_1(\tau/2)\,
\widetilde{\Phi}_2(\tau/2)\,\cdots\,\widetilde{\Phi}_{N-1}(\tau/2)\,
\widetilde{\Phi}_N(\tau)\,\widetilde{\Phi}_{N-1}(\tau/2)\,\cdots\,
\widetilde{\Phi}_2(\tau/2)\,\widetilde{\Phi}_1(\tau/2),
$$

*where $\widetilde{\Phi}_i$ is the axis-i lift. Then $S_N(\tau)$ converges*
*to $e^{\tau (L_1 + \cdots + L_N)}$ at global order $\min_i p_i$ on*
*compact time intervals.*

*Proof.* By induction on N. **Base case N = 2**: Theorem 7 (§10.3,
lines 2920-2984). **Inductive step**: assume the claim for N - 1; the
N-axis composition factors as $\widetilde{\Phi}_1(\tau/2)\,
S_{N-1}(\tau)\,\widetilde{\Phi}_1(\tau/2)$ where $S_{N-1}$ acts on
$\bigotimes_{i=2}^{N} H_i$ (regarding $H_1$ as a frozen parameter axis).
By Lemma 10.1, $\widetilde{\Phi}_1$ commutes with each $\widetilde{\Phi}_i$
($i \ge 2$); the inductive hypothesis gives $S_{N-1}(\tau) =
e^{\tau (L_2 + \cdots + L_N)} + O(\tau^{m + 1})$ with $m = \min_{i \ge 2} p_i$,
and the outer $\widetilde{\Phi}_1$ palindromic wrap inherits per-axis
order $p_1$ via Theorem 7's Step 4 (1D-on-2D extension by axis-frozen
sup-norm bound). Combining: $S_N(\tau) - e^{\tau (L_1 + \cdots + L_N)} =
O(\tau^{\min(p_1, m) + 1}) = O(\tau^{\min_i p_i + 1})$ per step, giving
global order $\min_i p_i$ via the Chernoff product theorem. ∎

**Remark 10.2 (no commutation bonus or penalty in N axes separable).**
The N-axis order claim $\mathrm{order}(S_N) = \min_i p_i$ inherits from
Theorem 7 verbatim — Remark 10.1 (line 2986) applies identically. The
3D separable splitting acquires no commutator-cancellation budget beyond
the per-axis inheritance; the order is **strictly limited by the weakest
axis** with no off-setting bonus for the additional axes.

#### 10.8.3 Strang3D composition rule (palindromic, X outermost)

The canonical 3D Strang composition with axes ordered (X, Y, Z) is the
**palindromic 5-leg**:

$$
S_{3D}(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau C}\,
e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2}.
\qquad (10.8.3)
$$

**Reduction theorem (NORMATIVE).** Under Lemma 10.1 pairwise commutation
(eq. 10.8.2),

$$
S_{3D}(\tau) \;=\; e^{\tau (A + B + C)} \;=\; e^{\tau L}
\quad \text{exactly},
\qquad (10.8.4)
$$

with **zero BCH residue**.

*Proof.* The five legs $\{e^{\tau A/2}, e^{\tau B/2}, e^{\tau C}, e^{\tau
B/2}, e^{\tau A/2}\}$ pairwise commute (since A, B, C do, by (10.8.2),
and exponentials of commuting operators commute). On commuting operators
the identity $e^X \cdot e^Y = e^{X + Y}$ holds, hence

$$
S_{3D}(\tau) = e^{\tau A / 2 + \tau B / 2 + \tau C + \tau B / 2 + \tau A / 2}
= e^{\tau (A + B + C)}.
$$ ∎

**Implications.**

1. The palindromic 5-leg form (10.8.3) is **bit-equal under exact
   arithmetic** to the asymmetric 3-leg form $e^{\tau A}\,e^{\tau B}\,
   e^{\tau C}$ and to any leg permutation. The type `Strang3D<X, Y, Z>`
   fixes the palindromic 5-leg ordering for **FP determinism**: identical
   leg sequence across architectures and compiler runs ensures bit-equal
   outputs at the cost of two extra leg evaluations vs the 3-leg form.
2. By Theorem 7' with N = 3 and (10.8.4), $\mathrm{order}(S_{3D}) =
   \min(\mathrm{order}(L_x), \mathrm{order}(L_y), \mathrm{order}(L_z))$;
   no commutator-bonus and no penalty (Remark 10.2).
3. The **5-leg vs 3-leg distinction is observably trivial in 3D
   separable** (bit-equal exact, ≤ a few ULP/node FP). It exists
   purely so the 3D path is structurally identical to v0.5.0
   `Strang2D` (5-leg X/Y/X-half-pattern symmetric in X), enabling code
   reuse of the per-axis half-step plumbing.

#### 10.8.4 Memory layout and indexing

**Storage**: row-major `Vec<f64>` of length $nx \cdot ny \cdot nz$, **x-fastest**.
The cell-index function is

$$
\mathrm{idx}(i, j, k) \;=\; k \cdot nx \cdot ny \;+\; j \cdot nx \;+\; i,
\qquad i \in [0, nx), \; j \in [0, ny), \; k \in [0, nz).
\qquad (10.8.6)
$$

This is the **inductive extension** of the v0.5.0 2D layout invariant I-T1
($\mathrm{idx}(i, j) = j \cdot nx + i$, x-fastest; see
`crates/semiflow-core/src/grid2d.rs:7-8`): adding a Z axis prepends a
$k \cdot nx \cdot ny$ stride while preserving the (i, j) layout of each
Z-slice as a v0.5.0 `GridFn2D`.

**Per-axis strides**:

| Axis | Stride | 1D-walk pattern (within `apply`) |
|------|--------|----------------------------------|
| X | $1$ | contiguous run of length $nx$ per (j, k) row |
| Y | $nx$ | strided run of length $ny$ per (i, k) column |
| Z | $nx \cdot ny$ | strided run of length $nz$ per (i, j) pillar |

Each per-axis lift becomes a 1D `apply` on the strided 1D view; the
existing v0.5.0 `AxisLift::X` and `AxisLift::Y` apply paths plug in
verbatim with the stride parameter, and the Z-axis adds a third stride
case (1, $nx$, $nx \cdot ny$ — the strides are constant in the inductive
extension by I-T1's row-major nature).

**Boundary policy reuse**: the v0.5.0 per-axis `BoundaryPolicy` enum
(`Reflect` / `ZeroExtend` / `LinearExtrapolate`) is reused **unchanged**
on the Z axis; no new variant is introduced. The 4-point cross-stencil
boundary rules of §10.7-bis / §10.7-ter (non-separable 2D regimes) are
**not invoked** in this section — §10.8 is the separable 3D base case.

#### 10.8.5 CFL aggregation (3D separable)

The 3D step bound is the strictest per-axis bound:

$$
\tau \;<\; \min\!\bigl( \tau_{\max}^x, \; \tau_{\max}^y, \; \tau_{\max}^z \bigr),
\qquad (10.8.7)
$$

with $\tau_{\max}^\ast$ the per-axis CFL of the corresponding leg
$L_\ast$ (e.g. for ζ-A `DiffusionChernoff`: $\tau_{\max}^x =
\mathrm{dx}^2 / (2 a_{\max}^x)$ and analogously per axis). No mixed-leg
CFL term appears in the separable case — that is the §10.7-bis / §10.7-ter
non-separable regime, where the cross-stencil contributes the
$4 \cdot \tau \cdot \|c\|_\infty < \mathrm{dx} \cdot \mathrm{dy}$ /
$\|\beta\|_\infty$ gate.

**Propagation**: a per-axis violation surfaces as
**`SemiflowError::CflViolated`** (ADR-0011) from the offending
`AxisLift3D::apply` — no new error variant. The third semantic field
overload of `CflViolated` (used in v0.7.0 / v0.9.0 Block A) is
**not** invoked here (separable 3D has no mixed-derivative CFL); the
existing `axis: Axis` field disambiguates which per-axis bound was
violated.

#### 10.8.6 NORMATIVE sympy gates (T10N_*)

Six sympy gates ratify the §10.8 claims symbolically (mirroring the T7N_*
and T9N_* convention of §10.7-bis.6 and §10.7-ter.6). All **NORMATIVE** —
the v0.9.0 Block C wave 2 verifier `verify_v0_9_0_3d_tensor.py` MUST exit
0 with all six passing.

| Gate | Statement |
|------|-----------|
| **T10N_pairwise_commute** | $[A, B] = [A, C] = [B, C] = 0$ symbolically (NC sympy symbols A, B, C with axis-disjoint commutation hypothesis applied via the Lemma 10.1 canonicaliser). |
| **T10N_strang3d_collapse** | Under T10N_pairwise_commute, $S_{3D}(\tau) = e^{\tau (A + B + C)}$ exactly (eq. 10.8.4) — no $\tau^k$ residue for any $k \ge 2$. |
| **T10N_palindrome** | The leg sequence $[A/2, B/2, C, B/2, A/2]$ equals its own reverse — static gate protecting against future refactor-induced reordering (analogous to T7N_palindrome / T9N_palindrome). |
| **T10N_oracle** | The 3D heat product Gaussian $u(t, x, y, z)$ (eq. 10.8.7-osc below) satisfies $\partial_t u = \tfrac12 (\partial_{xx} + \partial_{yy} + \partial_{zz}) u$ identically (constant-coefficient PDE consistency, sympy `simplify` to 0). |
| **T10N_zero-axis** | Setting $L_z \equiv 0$ (i.e. $C = 0$) collapses $S_{3D}(\tau) \bigm|_{C = 0}$ symbolically to $e^{\tau A / 2}\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,I\,e^{\tau B / 2}\,e^{\tau A / 2} = e^{\tau (A + B)}$, identical to the 3-leg `Strang2D` symbolic output (Lemma 10.1 N = 2 case). The implementation MUST detect this at construction and branch to the existing `Strang2D::apply` so the FP result is bit-equal to v0.5.0 `Strang2D` on the same per-axis legs. |
| **T10N_order_min** | Per Theorem 7' (§10.8.2), $\mathrm{order}(S_{3D}) = \min(\mathrm{order}(X), \mathrm{order}(Y), \mathrm{order}(Z))$. Verified by constructing three test cases (each axis the bottleneck in turn) and confirming the leading $\tau^k$ residue exponent matches the minimum per-axis order across all three. |

**Reuse note (NORMATIVE for the script)**: the v0.9.0 Block C wave 2
verifier reuses `canonicalize_AB(expr)` from the v0.7.0 verifier
(extended trivially to `canonicalize_ABC` by adding the (A, C) and
(B, C) commutator rewrite rules — symmetric copies of the (A, B) rule
structure). No new sympy machinery is required.

#### 10.8.7 G5_3D slope gate (NORMATIVE)

The end-to-end empirical slope gate ratifying $\mathrm{order}(S_{3D}) = 2$
under per-axis ζ-A `DiffusionChernoff` legs.

**Configuration**:

| Parameter | Value |
|-----------|-------|
| Domain | $\Omega = [-5, 5]^3$ |
| Final time | $T = 0.2$ |
| Time-step count | $n = 200$ (fixed across all probe N; CFL-safe at all probe grids — see CFL verification below) |
| Per-axis grid sizes | $N \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ (per-axis count; total cells $N^3 \in \{32768,\, 262144,\, 2097152,\, 16777216\}$) — recalibrated 2026-05-09; see "Pre-asymptote diagnosis" note below |
| Per-axis diffusion | $a_{xx} = a_{yy} = a_{zz} = 0.1$ (constant) |
| Per-axis legs | `DiffusionChernoff` (ζ-A, v0.3.0) on each of X, Y, Z |
| Initial datum | $u_0(x, y, z) = \exp(-(x^2 + y^2 + z^2))$ |
| Reference oracle | Closed-form 3D heat Gaussian (eq. 10.8.7-osc below) — exact, no high-resolution N_ref needed |
| Slope threshold | $\le -1.95$ (Strang-floor, identical to G3-strang-2D and G4_NS2D_aniso; UNCHANGED by 2026-05-09 recalibration) |
| Total per-step cost | $5 \cdot N^3$ leaf-leg cells |
| Total per-N cost | $5 \cdot 200 \cdot N^3 = 1000 N^3$ leaf-leg cells |
| Total gate cost (sum over basket) | $1000 \cdot (32^3 + 64^3 + 128^3 + 256^3) \approx 1.92 \times 10^{10}$ leaf-leg cells — wallclock dominated by the $N = 256$ leg ($\approx 50$ minutes on Intel i7-12700K, AVX2, `--features parallel,simd,slow-tests --release`) |

**Closed-form 3D Gaussian oracle** (constant-coefficient case
$a_{xx} = a_{yy} = a_{zz} = a$, here $a = 0.1$):

$$
u(t, x, y, z) \;=\;
\frac{1}{(1 + 4at)^{3/2}}\,
\exp\!\Bigl( -\frac{x^2 + y^2 + z^2}{1 + 4at} \Bigr),
\qquad
u(0, x, y, z) \;=\; e^{-(x^2 + y^2 + z^2)},
\qquad (10.8.7\text{-osc})
$$

derived as the tensor product of three 1D heat-kernel oracles with
$\sigma_0 = 1/\sqrt{2}$ (so that $u_0 = e^{-x^2}$ and $\sigma_0^2 = 1/2$)
and $\sigma^2(t) = \sigma_0^2 + 2at = 1/2 + 2at$ per axis, giving
per-axis variance $1 + 4at$ in the denominator of the exponent
(and the 3D normalisation factor is $(1 + 4at)^{-3/2}$, matching
eq. (10.8.7-osc) above). **Crucially, this oracle is exact at arbitrary N**:
unlike the v0.9.0 Block A G4_NS2D_aniso gate (which required a
high-resolution reference simulation since no closed form exists for
non-trivial $\beta(x, y)$), the 3D constant-coefficient Gaussian admits a
closed-form ground truth and **no separate N_ref simulation is needed** —
strictly cheaper than the 4-point 2D basket.

**CFL verification**: at $a = 0.1$ per axis and $\Omega = [-5, 5]$ with
$N = 256$ (finest probe in the recalibrated basket), $\mathrm{dx} =
10/255 \approx 0.0392$, so $\tau_{\max} = \mathrm{dx}^2 / (2 \cdot 0.1)
\approx 7.69 \times 10^{-3}$. With $\tau = T / n = 0.2 / 200 = 0.001$,
the CFL margin is $\sim 7.7\times$ at the finest grid (and grows by
$\sim 4\times$ per $N$ halving — easily satisfied at $N = 128, 64, 32$).
The fixed $n = 200$ is therefore CFL-safe across the entire
$\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ basket without $N$-dependent step refinement.

**Pre-asymptote diagnosis (2026-05-09 recalibration, NORMATIVE)**: the
original v0.9.0-design basket $\{16, 32, 64\}$ included one
**under-resolved point**: at $N = 16$, $\mathrm{dx} = 10/15 \approx 0.667$
spans only $\sim 2$ grid points across the half-width
$\sigma = 1/\sqrt{2} \approx 0.707$ of the Gaussian initial datum, placing
$N = 16$ in the **pre-asymptotic regime** where the spatial cubic-Hermite
interpolation has not yet entered $O(\mathrm{dx}^2)$ rate. The first
prod-HW run (Intel i7-12700K, 2026-05-09; deferred from v0.9.0 release
wave per Block C ship note) measured per-$N$ errors $\{2.37 \times 10^{-2},
\, 1.51 \times 10^{-2},\, 4.50 \times 10^{-3}\}$ at $\{16, 32, 64\}$,
ratios $1.57$ / $3.36$, $\log_2$ progression $0.65 \to 1.75$ — monotonically
ascending toward the order-2 asymptote but not at it (collapsed OLS slope
$-1.198$, fails $\le -1.95$ by $-0.75$). Recalibrate the basket to
$\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$, mirroring the v0.9.0 G4_NS2D_aniso 2D
self-convergence redesign (commit `0180292`, §10.7-ter.7 — same
"skip-the-coarsest-pre-asymptotic-point" convention: drop $N = 32$ from
2D OLS, drop $N = 16$ from 3D OLS); the gate threshold $\le -1.95$ is
**unchanged** (the basket move into the asymptotic regime is precisely
where the order-2 floor is achievable). See `audit-findings-v0_11_0.md`
for the raw per-$N$ diagnostic data; see ADR-0024 Amendment 2026-05-09
for the architectural ratification. Empirical pre-asymptote first
observed in v0.11.0 prod-HW run (i7-12700K, 2026-05-09).

**Slope gate**: an OLS regression of $\log_2 \|S_{3D}^n u_0 - u(T, \cdot)\|_\infty$
on $\log_2 N$ (over the recalibrated basket $N \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}$)
yields a slope in the open neighbourhood of $-2$ (the Strang-floor),
empirically extrapolated to $\approx -1.95$ to $-2.00$ from the
$\log_2$-ratio progression at the original basket; the NORMATIVE
acceptance threshold is

$$
\mathrm{slope}_{\mathrm{OLS}} \;\le\; -1.95.
\qquad (10.8.7\text{-gate})
$$

This exercises the full Strang3D path end-to-end (per-axis Chernoff legs,
AxisLift3D / Axis::Z dispatch, row-major 3D index correctness, per-axis
strided 1D walks at strides 1 / nx / nx·ny, palindromic 5-leg reduction
at FP precision) on a **non-trivial 3D field** ($N^3$ cells with all three
axes active, the smallest nontrivial reduction-degenerate input would be
a Y-Z-independent test that §10.4 Lemma 10.2 already covers in 2D and
which the engineer SHOULD include as a regression sub-gate at $N = 32$).

#### 10.8.8 Cross-references

- §10.3 Theorem 7 — N=2 base case for the Theorem 7' induction.
- §10.4 Lemma 10.2 — Y-independent reduction; the analogous Z-independent
  reduction in 3D (`f(x, y, z) = g(x, y)`) reduces $S_{3D}$ to $S_{2D}$
  bit-equal modulo FP, providing a strong reduction oracle for 3D
  acceptance gates and a Block C wave 2 implementation regression target.
- §10.5 G3-strang-2D — parent slope gate; G5_3D mirrors its design with a
  4-point basket $\{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ (recalibrated 2026-05-09 from the
  original 3-point $\{16, 32, 64\}$ — see "Pre-asymptote diagnosis" note
  in §10.8.7 and ADR-0024 Amendment 2026-05-09).
- §10.7 — out-of-scope deferral (line 3091-3093): "**3D and higher**: the
  same construction extends inductively but is not part of v0.5.0 scope".
  This §10.8 fulfils the deferral.
- §10.7-bis, §10.7-ter — non-separable 2D regimes (scalar $c$ and
  anisotropic $\beta$); 3D non-separable is deferred to v1.0+ as a
  separate ADR (mirroring the v0.5→v0.7 separable→non-separable
  progression in 2D).
- ADR-0012 — v0.5.0 2D foundation; ADR-0024 — this 3D extension;
  ADR-0011 — `SemiflowError::CflViolated` reused, no new variants.
- `verify_v0_9_0_3d_tensor.py` — Block C wave 2 engineer verifier
  (six T10N_* gates + G5_3D slope gate).
- `contracts/semiflow-core.tensor.yaml` — Phase 1 struct schema (to be
  amended by Block C wave 2 engineer with `Grid3D`, `GridFn3D`,
  `AxisLift3D` or `Axis::Z`, and `Strang3D<X, Y, Z>` schemas;
  `total_additions` 7 → 11).
- `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` — six new T10N_* properties
  plus G5_3D, all `severity: NORMATIVE`, to be added by Block C wave 2.

---

### 10.9 1D parallelism — bit-equality guarantee (v0.12.0, ADR-0036)

For each 1D Chernoff
approximant $T_\tau$ on grid $\{x_i\}_{i=0}^{n-1}$, the output value
$u_\tau(x_i)$ is a closed-form function of $\{u(x_j) : j \in \mathcal{N}(i)\}$
for a fixed stencil neighbourhood $\mathcal{N}(i)$ (width $\leq 9$ for
the 6th-order diffusion case; pointwise / non-local for `ShiftChernoff1D`
and `DriftReactionChernoff`). The parallel implementation partitions
$\{0, \ldots, n-1\}$ into disjoint contiguous chunks
$I_k = [k \cdot c,\; \min((k+1) c,\; n))$ with $c = \lceil n / n_{\text{thr}} \rceil$,
evaluates each chunk in a separate thread, and writes to non-overlapping
output slots. No floating-point reductions cross thread boundaries; therefore
every f64 written to the parallel output buffer is the result of an
identical sequence of floating-point operations as in the serial path.
Byte-equality is preserved across thread counts in $\{1, 2, 4, 8\}$ —
enforced by the release-blocking gate `chernoff1d_parallel_bit_equal`
(`tests/chernoff1d_parallel_bit_equal.rs`, feature `parallel` $\wedge$
`slow-tests`). See ADR-0036.

---

## 11. Adaptive PI step controller (v0.6.0, ADR-0014)

**Status**: NORMATIVE for v0.6.0. Adds `AdaptivePI<C>` as a generic
**semigroup-splitting integrator** — not a `ChernoffFunction`. The
distinction is operationally important and is documented here for the
benefit of downstream callers and verification scripts.

### 11.1 Semigroup-splitting interpretation (NORMATIVE)

`AdaptivePI<C>` wraps any inner `C: ChernoffFunction` and computes an
approximation of $e^{T A} f_0$ on a target time interval $[0, T]$ by an
**adaptively-spaced sequence of substeps**

$$
0 \;=\; t_0 < t_1 < t_2 < \cdots < t_N \;=\; T,
$$

where the substep widths $\tau_i := t_{i+1} - t_i$ are produced
*online* by the PI controller (§11.2 below) and the substep count $N$
is **runtime-determined** — there is no fixed $n$ as in
$(C(T/n))^n f_0$. The integrator action is

$$
\boxed{\;
u_{i+1} \;:=\; (C.\mathrm{apply})(\tau_i,\, u_i)
\;\;\approx\;\; e^{\tau_i A}\,u_i \;+\; O(\tau_i^{p+1}) \quad (\text{per substep, local}),
\;}
$$

where $p := C.\mathrm{order}()$ is the per-step local truncation order
of the inner Chernoff function (`p = 2` for ζ-A / ζ⁴ / TruncatedExp / TruncatedExp⁴
in v0.6.0; `p = 4` only when the inner is a sympathetic 4th-order
substep — a forward-compatibility hook).

#### §11.1.bis Axis distinction (NORMATIVE clarification, v0.6.1)

Two orthogonal accuracy axes coexist in this contract and they MUST NOT
be conflated:

- **τ-axis** (time) — `ChernoffFunction::order() -> u32` returns the
  per-step Chernoff consistency order $p$ such that single-step error is
  $\bigl\|S(\tau)f - \sum_{k=0}^{p} \tau^k A^k f / k!\bigr\| = O(\tau^{p+1})$,
  and the global Lady-Windermere fan accumulation gives error
  $O(\tau_{\max}^p)$ over $N \approx T/\tau_{\max}$ substeps (see §11.1
  derivation above). This is the ONLY quantity advertised by `order()`.
- **dx-axis** (space) — the spatial finite-difference truncation order
  $q$ of the underlying stencil (e.g. $O(dx^2)$ for `DiffusionChernoff`
  ζ-A's 5-point central FD on $f^{(k)}$; $O(dx^4)$ for
  `Diffusion4thChernoff` and `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff`'s Fornberg
  7-point central / 5-point divergence-form stencils per §9.2.4 and
  §9.2.5). $q$ is a SEPARATE, ORTHOGONAL property of the discretisation
  and is **not** advertised by `order()`. Spatial accuracy is observable
  only via the convergence-slope gates G3 / G3⁴ (1D) and G3-2D / G3⁴-2D
  (2D) — see `properties.yaml` and §9.6 / §10.5 / §10.6.

The `AdaptivePI<C>` controller's Richardson divisor $2^p - 1$ and PI
gains $\alpha = 0.7/p, \beta = 0.4/p$ (§11.2 below) are **derived from
the τ-axis $p$ only** — substituting $q$ here would break the
local-error estimator's denominator and the PI feedback law.

For `Diffusion4thChernoff` and `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff`, $p = 2$
(τ-axis Chernoff consistency, identical to v0.5.0 ζ-A and v0.4.0 TruncatedExp
because the γ-A baseline / Strang composition / K=4 truncated power
series all saturate Chernoff order at 2) and $q = 4$ (dx-axis spatial
accuracy at constant $a$, which is the regime of the v0.6.0 release
gate G3⁴-2D — see ADR-0013 §3 and the Mickens 1994 §3.2 impossibility
note for variable-$a$ residue $O(dx^2)$). The names `Diffusion4thChernoff`
and `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff` refer to the **spatial** accuracy $q$,
not to the τ-axis order.

This clarification is NORMATIVE for v0.6.1 (PATCH). Motivating
incident: `docs/audit-findings-v0_6_0.md` D1 — the v0.6.0 implementations
of `Diffusion4thChernoff::order()` and `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff::order()`
returned `4`, conflating $q$ with $p$ and propagating an incorrect
$2^4 - 1 = 15$ Richardson divisor through `AdaptivePI` (the correct
divisor is $2^2 - 1 = 3$, matching the inner Chernoff order). v0.6.1
fixes the implementation to return `2`, restoring agreement with this
contract clause.

**Convergence of $u_N \to e^{T A} f_0$ as $\tau_{\max} \to 0$** is
governed by the standard **Lady-Windermere fan accumulation argument**
(Hairer–Lubich–Wanner *Geometric Numerical Integration*, §II.3):

$$
\|u_N - e^{T A} f_0\|_\infty \;\le\; \sum_{i=0}^{N-1} M\,e^{\omega(T-t_i)}\,\|(C.\mathrm{apply})(\tau_i, u_i) - e^{\tau_i A} u_i\|_\infty
\;\le\; M\,T\,e^{\omega T} \cdot O(\tau_{\max}^p),
$$

i.e. **global error $O(\tau_{\max}^p)$** under quasi-contractivity
$\|S(\tau)\| \le M e^{\omega \tau}$ — note this is the per-step LOCAL
order $p+1$ accumulating to GLOBAL $p$ over $N \approx T/\tau$
substeps. Crucially, **this is NOT Theorem 6's** $O(1/n)$ bound, which
applies only to the *fixed-step* iterate $(C(T/n))^n$. The Theorem-6
hypotheses (order, growth, quasi-contractivity) do still play a role:
they imply local order $p+1$ per substep, which feeds the Lady-Windermere
fan accumulation into the global $O(\tau_{\max}^p)$ bound.

**Why `AdaptivePI` is NOT a `ChernoffFunction`**: the `ChernoffFunction`
trait requires a fixed `order(): u32` reported at construction and a
fixed-`n` iteration semantics via `ChernoffSemigroup<C>::evolve(t, f)
= (C.apply(t/n))^n f`. `AdaptivePI` violates both: the substep count
$N$ is runtime, and the *effective* order is the inner $p$ — but only
in the asymptotic sense above, not as a `Chernoff::order()` advertised
value. Implementing the trait would require lying about either; the
v0.6.0 design instead **does NOT implement `ChernoffFunction`** for
`AdaptivePI<C>`, and the inner $C$'s order is exposed via
`AdaptivePI::inner_order() -> u32` (forward-pass through to
`func.order()`). The usage pattern is

```rust
let pi = AdaptivePI::new(magnus4_chernoff)
    .with_tol(1e-8, 1e-6);
let outcome = pi.evolve_adaptive(T, &f0)?;
let u_T = outcome.final_state;
```

NOT

```rust
// WRONG — AdaptivePI is not a ChernoffFunction.
let semigroup = ChernoffSemigroup::new(pi, 100)?;
```

### 11.2 PI controller (Söderlind 2002)

Per substep, the controller:

1. **Forms the half-step Richardson estimator**. Given current
   $(u_i, \tau)$:
   - $u_{\mathrm{full}} := C.\mathrm{apply}(\tau, u_i)$;
   - $u_{\mathrm{half\_1}} := C.\mathrm{apply}(\tau/2, u_i)$;
   - $u_{\mathrm{half}}   := C.\mathrm{apply}(\tau/2, u_{\mathrm{half\_1}})$.

   The local-truncation difference is

   $$
   \mathrm{err}_i \;:=\; \frac{\|u_{\mathrm{half}} - u_{\mathrm{full}}\|_\infty}{2^p - 1},
   $$

   where the denominator $2^p - 1 \in \{1, 3, 7, 15, 31, 63\}$ for
   $p \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6\}$ comes from Richardson extrapolation
   under the assumption that local truncation is $C \cdot \tau^{p+1} +
   O(\tau^{p+2})$:

   $$
   u_{\mathrm{full}} - e^{\tau A} u_i \approx C\,\tau^{p+1}, \qquad
   u_{\mathrm{half}} - e^{\tau A} u_i \approx C\,2 \cdot (\tau/2)^{p+1} = C\,\tau^{p+1}/2^p,
   $$
   $$
   u_{\mathrm{half}} - u_{\mathrm{full}} \approx C\,\tau^{p+1}\,(1/2^p - 1) = -C\,\tau^{p+1}\,(2^p - 1)/2^p,
   $$

   so $|u_{\mathrm{half}} - u_{\mathrm{full}}| / (2^p - 1) \approx
   C\,\tau^{p+1}/2^p$ — a tight estimator of the half-step local
   truncation magnitude, off by a factor of $2^p$ which is absorbed
   into the safety factor `safety = 0.9`.

2. **Forms the mixed tolerance** (relative + absolute, NORMATIVE):

   $$
   \mathrm{tol}_i \;:=\; \mathrm{tol}_{\mathrm{abs}} \;+\; \mathrm{tol}_{\mathrm{rel}} \cdot \max\bigl(\|u_i\|_\infty,\, \|u_{\mathrm{full}}\|_\infty\bigr).
   $$

   The default constants are $\mathrm{tol}_{\mathrm{abs}} = 10^{-8}$
   and $\mathrm{tol}_{\mathrm{rel}} = 10^{-6}$ — chosen so that for
   bounded smooth solutions ($\|u\|_\infty \approx 1$) the relative
   floor dominates ($\mathrm{tol} \approx 10^{-6}$) but for vanishing
   amplitudes the absolute floor prevents division-by-zero.

3. **Computes the new step** via the PI controller (Söderlind 2002,
   "PI.4.7" parameter set; HLW §IV.2):

   $$
   \boxed{\;
   \tau_{\mathrm{new}} \;:=\; \mathrm{clamp}\Bigl(\;
       \tau \cdot \mathrm{safety} \cdot \bigl(\tfrac{\mathrm{tol}_i}{\mathrm{err}_i}\bigr)^{\alpha} \cdot \bigl(\tfrac{\mathrm{err}_{i-1}}{\mathrm{err}_i}\bigr)^{\beta}
   \;,\; \mathrm{min\_ratio} \cdot \tau \;,\; \mathrm{max\_ratio} \cdot \tau\Bigr),
   \;}
   $$

   with $\alpha = 0.7/p, \beta = 0.4/p$ (the PI.4.7 set; $\beta = 0$
   reduces to the classical Richardson "I" controller, but $\beta > 0$
   smooths out high-frequency oscillation in $\tau$ at minor stability
   cost — Söderlind 2002 §3 documents ~30% rejection-rate reduction at
   matched accuracy for diffusion-dominated semigroups). Default
   $\mathrm{min\_ratio} = 0.2,\, \mathrm{max\_ratio} = 5.0,\, \mathrm{safety} = 0.9$.
   The $\mathrm{err}_{i-1}$ on the first substep is initialised to
   $\mathrm{err}_0 = \mathrm{err}_i$ (so the $(\mathrm{err}_{i-1}/\mathrm{err}_i)^\beta$
   factor is $1$ and the controller reduces to pure-I on substep 0).

4. **Decides accept/reject**:
   - If $\mathrm{err}_i \le \mathrm{tol}_i$: ACCEPT, set
     $u_{i+1} := u_{\mathrm{half}}$ (the more accurate of the two
     trials), advance $t_{i+1} := t_i + \tau$, set the next trial step
     to $\tau_{\mathrm{new}}$.
   - If $\mathrm{err}_i > \mathrm{tol}_i$: REJECT, retry the same
     substep with $\tau \leftarrow \tau_{\mathrm{new}}$ (the controller
     guarantees $\tau_{\mathrm{new}} < \tau$ in this branch).

### 11.3 Termination guarantees and runaway protection

The controller is bounded multiplicatively: $\tau_{\mathrm{new}} /
\tau \in [\mathrm{min\_ratio}, \mathrm{max\_ratio}] = [0.2, 5.0]$, so
in the *worst case* of repeated rejection at $\tau_{\mathrm{new}} =
0.2\,\tau$ the substep contracts geometrically. After $k$ rejections,
$\tau \le 5\,\tau_0 \cdot 0.2^k$, so $k \ge \log_5(\tau_0 /
\tau_{\min\_useful}) / \log_5(5) = \log_5(\tau_0 / \tau_{\min\_useful})$
rejections suffice to reach any caller-meaningful $\tau_{\min\_useful}$.
Pathological cases (tolerance unreachable in floating-point regardless
of $\tau$) trigger the runaway hard cap: when
$\mathrm{steps\_attempted} \ge \mathrm{max\_substeps}$ (default
$10^5$) the integrator returns

$$
\mathrm{Err}\bigl(\mathrm{SemiflowError::AdaptiveStepRejected}\,\{\,
  \mathrm{last\_tau}\,,\; \mathrm{last\_err}\,,\; \mathrm{steps\_attempted}\,\}\bigr).
$$

This is a **NEW error variant** in `errors.yaml` v0.5.0; payload triple
allows the caller to diagnose the failure mode (controller pinned at
$\tau \approx 10^{-15}$ ⇒ tol unreachable; or $\mathrm{err}$ ≫ $\mathrm{tol}$
⇒ inner $C$ may be discontinuous in $u$).

### 11.4 Composability with `Strang2D` and 2D states

`AdaptivePI<C>` is generic over `C: ChernoffFunction`, so
`AdaptivePI<Strang2D<C_x, C_y>>` instantiates directly when both inner
1D Chernoff functions implement the trait. The `State` trait's
`axpy/scale/norm_sup/zeroed_like` methods (math.md §1.3) apply uniformly
to `GridFn1D` and `GridFn2D`, so the half-step Richardson buffers are
allocated lazily via `func.apply` — no 2D-specific code path is needed
in `AdaptivePI`.

**Cross-references**:

- ADR-0014 — architectural decision record.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.traits.yaml` — `AdaptivePI<C>` and
  `AdaptiveOutcome<S>` struct entries.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.errors.yaml` — `AdaptiveStepRejected` variant.
- `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` — `G_PI` (efficiency vs. fixed
  step on stiff CEV) and `adaptive_pi_contractivity` (proptest gate).
- Söderlind, "Automatic control and adaptive time-stepping",
  *Numerical Algorithms* **31** (2002) 281–310.
- Hairer, Lubich, Wanner, *Geometric Numerical Integration* (2nd ed.,
  Springer 2006). §II.3 (Lady Windermere's fan / local-truncation
  accumulation), §IV.2 (step-size control).

## 7. Glossary

| Term                | Definition |
|---------------------|------------|
| Chernoff function   | Strongly continuous family $S(\tau)$ with $S(0)=I$, $S'(0)$ closable to a generator. |
| Chernoff approximation | The iterate $(S(t/n))^n f$. |
| Heat kernel of Gaussian | The exact solution $(1+2t)^{-1/2} e^{-x^2/(1+2t)}$ — v0.1.0 oracle. |
| Advection-diffusion oracle | $u(t,x) = (1+2t)^{-1/2} \exp(-(x+t/2)^2/(1+2t))$ — v0.2.0 oracle (§9.5). |
| Mehler kernel       | Kernel of Ornstein–Uhlenbeck semigroup. **Not used in v0.1.0/v0.2.0** (M1). |
| Operator splitting  | Decomposition $L = A + B$ with separate Chernoff approximants for each piece (§9.1). |
| Strang composition  | $\Phi(\tau) = D(\tau/2)\,R(\tau)\,D(\tau/2)$ — palindromic, second-order (§9.4). |
| Quasi-contractivity | $\|S(\tau)\| \le M e^{\omega \tau}$. |
| Sup-norm            | $\|f\|_\infty = \sup_x |f(x)|$. v0.1.0 default error norm. |

---

## §12 — Graph PDE — discrete heat semigroup on finite weighted graphs (NORMATIVE library choices; CITATION-only mathematics)

This section documents the mathematical foundations for `GraphHeatChernoff<F>` introduced in v2.1 Wave A. It contains **no new theorems**. Every mathematical statement is either a citation of an established result — restated verbatim in our notation — or a NORMATIVE library choice pinning a specific API or data-layout invariant. See ADR-0049 for the decision rationale.

### §12.1 — Setting: finite weighted graph and its Laplacian (NORMATIVE)

A **finite simple weighted undirected graph** is a triple `G = (V, E, w)` where:

- `V = {0, 1, …, N − 1}` is the node set, `|V| = N`.
- `E ⊆ { (u, v) : u, v ∈ V, u ≠ v }` (unordered pairs; no self-loops).
- `w : E → (0, ∞)` assigns a strictly positive finite weight to each edge.

**State space.** The natural Hilbert space is `ℓ²(V) ≅ ℝ^N` with inner product `⟨f, g⟩ = Σ_{i∈V} f(i) g(i)`. In v2.1 we ship real-valued types only (`F = f64`); complex-valued generalisation is deferred.

**Combinatorial Laplacian.** The matrix `L_G ∈ ℝ^{N×N}` is defined entry-wise by

```
L_G[i, j] = { −w(i, j)        if (i, j) ∈ E
            { deg_w(i)         if i = j
            { 0                otherwise
```

where `deg_w(i) = Σ_{j : (i,j) ∈ E} w(i, j)` is the weighted degree. `L_G` is symmetric positive semidefinite with smallest eigenvalue `λ_0 = 0` (constant eigenvector) and largest eigenvalue `λ_{N−1} ≤ 2 · max_i deg_w(i)` (Gershgorin; see §12.4).

**Symmetric normalised Laplacian** (opt-in, ADR-0048). With degree matrix `D = diag(deg_w)`,

```
L_sym = I − D^{−½} W D^{−½}
```

where `W` is the adjacency matrix `W[i,j] = w(i,j)` for `(i,j) ∈ E`, zero otherwise. Eigenvalues of `L_sym` lie in `[0, 2]` (Chung 1997 §1.3 Lemma 1.7). In v2.1 `GraphHeatChernoff` uses the combinatorial Laplacian by default; normalised variant is deferred to v2.2.

**CSR storage layout (NORMATIVE — also ADR-0048).** `Laplacian<F>` stores `L_G` in compressed sparse row format with three `Vec` fields:

| Field       | Type           | Length   | Invariant |
|-------------|----------------|----------|-----------|
| `row_ptr`   | `Vec<u32>`     | `N + 1`  | `row_ptr[0] = 0`; `row_ptr[N] = nnz`; non-strictly monotonic |
| `col_idx`   | `Vec<u32>`     | `nnz`    | Each row's entries sorted ascending; no duplicate column in a row |
| `vals`      | `Vec<F>`       | `nnz`    | All finite (`f64::is_finite`); all `col_idx[k] < N` |

**Symmetric storage**: each undirected edge `(u, v)` contributes two entries — `(u, v)` in row `u` and `(v, u)` in row `v`. Hence `nnz = 2|E| + N` (off-diagonal pairs + diagonal entries). **Diagonal-last invariant**: for each row `i`, the diagonal entry `L_G[i, i] = deg_w(i)` is stored as the last element in the row's slice (column `i` is the largest column index in the row after sorting, guaranteed because `L_G[i, j] ≠ 0` only for `j ∈ N(i) ∪ {i}` and we require `j < i` for at least one neighbour or the diagonal stands alone). Implementation: `crates/semiflow-core/src/graph.rs` `Laplacian::from_edges`.

The CSR layout is immutable post-assembly (no in-place re-weighting after construction). This is a NORMATIVE contract: code that relies on mutating `row_ptr`, `col_idx`, or `vals` after `Laplacian::from_edges` returns invokes undefined behaviour from `semiflow-core`'s perspective.

### §12.2 — Chernoff product formula on `ℝ^N` (CITATION)

> **Theorem (Chernoff product formula — Pazy 1983, §1.3, Theorem 1.3, p. 19;
> Engel-Nagel 2000, §III.5, Theorem 5.2, p. 220; Chernoff 1968, *J. Funct. Anal.*
> 2:238-242).** Let `A` be the generator of a `C_0`-semigroup `T(t)` on a Banach
> space `X` with `‖T(t)‖ ≤ M e^{ωt}`. Let `S : [0, ∞) → ℒ(X)` be strongly
> continuous with `S(0) = I` and `‖S(τ)‖ ≤ M e^{ωτ}` for all `τ ≥ 0`. If
> `S'(0) f = A f` for all `f` in a core `D ⊂ D(A)`, then for every `t > 0`
>
> ```
>   lim_{n→∞} (S(t/n))^n f = T(t) f      (strong convergence).
> ```
>
> Quantitative bound: `‖(S(t/n))^n f − T(t) f‖ = O(1/n)` for `f ∈ D(A²)`.

**This section restates published classical results in our notation; no new theorem is claimed.**

**Specialisation to `X = ℝ^N`, `A = −L_G`.** Because `L_G` is an `N×N` matrix it is bounded, so `D(A) = D(A²) = ℝ^N` (Pazy 1983, §1.3, Theorem 1.3 bounded generator case). The semigroup `T(t) = e^{−t L_G}` is the matrix exponential, a contraction on `(ℝ^N, ℓ²)` because `L_G ⪰ 0`. The abstract Chernoff product formula applies in **operator norm** (not merely strongly), because finite-dimensional operator-norm topology equals strong topology. Convergence rate is therefore `O(1/n)` in the spectral norm `‖ · ‖_2` uniformly over initial conditions.

**Foundational citations:**

- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, J. Funct. Anal. **2** (1968) 238-242. DOI 10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7. (Original result.)
- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to Partial Differential Equations*, Springer 1983. §1.3, Theorem 1.3 (p. 19): bounded generator implies semigroup is matrix exponential; §1.5 Corollary 1.11: operator-norm convergence of Euler product.
- K.-J. Engel, R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations*, Springer 2000. §III.5, Theorem 5.2 (p. 220): Chernoff product formula with quantitative bound.

### §12.3 — Order-1 leading Chernoff `S(τ) = I − τ L_G` — hypothesis verification (CITATION + NORMATIVE)

**Definition (NORMATIVE).** The leading-order Chernoff approximant for the graph heat semigroup is

```
S(τ) : ℝ^N → ℝ^N,    S(τ) f = f − τ L_G f = (I − τ L_G) f.
```

This defines `GraphHeatChernoff<F>::apply_into(scratch, dst, tau, src)` in `crates/semiflow-core/src/graph_heat.rs`. The function signature is NORMATIVE: `apply_into` takes a mutable scratch slice, mutable destination slice, step `τ`, and immutable source slice, and writes `(I − τ L_G) src` into `dst` in a single CSR matrix-vector product. No heap allocation occurs inside `apply_into`.

**Hypothesis verification for the Chernoff product formula (§12.2):**

1. `S(0) f = f − 0 · L_G f = f` for all `f` — trivial. ✓
2. `τ ↦ S(τ) f` is strongly continuous — it is affine-linear in `τ`. ✓
3. `S'(0) f = (d/dτ)|_{τ=0} (f − τ L_G f) = −L_G f` — matches generator `A = −L_G`. ✓ (CITATION: Engel-Nagel 2000, §III.5, Theorem 5.2 hypothesis check.)
4. `S(τ)` is quasi-contractive — see §12.4 for the stability envelope. ✓

Therefore, by §12.2, `(S(t/n))^n f → e^{−t L_G} f` in operator norm as `n → ∞`, with rate `O(1/n)` for any `f ∈ ℝ^N`.

**Order of approximation.** By Taylor expansion, `e^{−τ L_G} = I − τ L_G + ½ τ² L_G² + O(τ³)`, so `S(τ) = e^{−τ L_G} + O(τ²)`. The leading Chernoff is therefore first-order accurate in a single step. Global error on `[0, t]` with `n` steps is `O(t/n)` = `O(1/n)` for fixed `t`. (CITATION: Pazy 1983, §1.5, Corollary 1.11; Engel-Nagel 2000, §III.5, Remark 5.3.)

### §12.4 — `GraphHeatChernoff` implementation and stability envelope (NORMATIVE)

**Stability envelope (NORMATIVE).** `semiflow-core` does not clamp `τ` internally. The caller is responsible for choosing `τ` within the quasi-contractivity window. Operator-norm contractivity (`‖S(τ)‖_{op} ≤ 1`) is guaranteed if and only if

```
τ · ρ̄ ≤ ½,          where  ρ̄ = max_{i ∈ V}  Σ_{j} |L_G[i, j]|.
```

Here `ρ̄` is the **Gershgorin upper bound on the spectral radius** of `L_G` (CITATION: R. S. Varga, *Matrix Iterative Analysis*, Springer 2000, §1.5, Theorem 1.11; also F. L. Bauer, C. T. Fike, *Norms and exclusion theorems*, Numer. Math. **2** (1960) 137-141). For the combinatorial Laplacian, `ρ̄ = max_i deg_w(i) + max_i deg_w(i) = 2 · max_i deg_w(i)` (diagonal plus row-sum of off-diagonal absolute values equals twice the weighted degree). Hence the contractivity condition simplifies to `τ ≤ 1 / (2 · max_i deg_w(i))`.

**`Laplacian::spectral_radius_bound() → F`** returns `ρ̄` so that callers can compute the recommended `τ_max = 0.5 / ρ̄`. This is a NORMATIVE API contract (ADR-0047).

**Quasi-contractivity parameters (NORMATIVE).** `GraphHeatChernoff::growth() → (M, ω)` returns `(1.0, ρ̄)`. The pair satisfies `‖S(τ)‖ ≤ M e^{ω τ}` for all `τ ≥ 0` because `‖(I − τ L_G)‖ ≤ 1 + τ λ_{N−1} ≤ e^{τ λ_{N−1}} ≤ e^{τ ρ̄}` via `1 + x ≤ e^x`. (CITATION: Engel-Nagel 2000, §III.5, Corollary 5.5.) Outside the `½ ρ̄^{−1}` window, Chernoff convergence still holds by this exponential bound, but the iterates are no longer contractive — they grow before cancelling. This regime is documented in ADR-0047 §"Quasi-contractivity outside stability window" and is the caller's responsibility.

**`apply_into` NORMATIVE contract.** Signature:

```rust
fn apply_into(&self, _scratch: &mut [F], dst: &mut [F], tau: F, src: &[F]);
```

- `src.len() == dst.len() == n_nodes` — panics if violated.
- `dst[i] = src[i] − τ · (L_G · src)[i]` for all `i` — single CSR SpMV, no approximation.
- `_scratch` is unused in the scalar path; reserved for future SIMD/parallel paths.
- One call represents one Chernoff step; `n` calls with `τ = t / n` converge to `e^{−t L_G} src`.

### §12.5 — CSR storage layout and invariants (NORMATIVE — see ADR-0048)

This sub-section mirrors ADR-0048 verbatim so that `contracts/semiflow-core.math.md` is self-contained for readers consulting only the math contract.

**CSR invariants (NORMATIVE):**

1. `row_ptr.len() == n_nodes + 1`, `row_ptr[0] == 0`, `row_ptr[n_nodes] == col_idx.len() == vals.len()` (= `nnz`).
2. `row_ptr` is non-strictly monotonically non-decreasing.
3. For each row `i`, `col_idx[row_ptr[i]..row_ptr[i+1]]` is strictly sorted ascending with no duplicate column index.
4. No self-loops in `Graph<F>`. In `Laplacian<F>`, the diagonal entry `L_G[i, i] = deg_w(i)` is the **last** entry in each row's column slice (diagonal-last invariant). This is enforced by `Laplacian::from_edges` which sorts each row ascending and then appends the diagonal.
5. All `vals[k]` are finite (`f64::is_finite(vals[k]) == true` for all `k`). All `col_idx[k] < n_nodes`.
6. **Immutable post-assembly.** `row_ptr`, `col_idx`, and `vals` are private fields; no public mutation API is exposed after `Laplacian::from_edges` returns.

**Symmetric storage convention.** Each undirected edge `(u, v) ∈ E` is stored twice: once as off-diagonal entry `(u, v)` in row `u` and once as `(v, u)` in row `v`. Total `nnz = 2|E| + N` (two off-diagonal entries per edge plus `N` diagonal entries).

**Relationship to §12.1 definition.** The CSR `vals` array encodes exactly the matrix `L_G` defined in §12.1: negative edge weights on off-diagonal positions and positive weighted degrees on the diagonal. A read of `vals[k]` for a diagonal position always yields a non-negative value; a read for an off-diagonal position always yields a non-positive value (because `w > 0`). These sign conventions are NORMATIVE and tested by `crates/semiflow-core/src/graph.rs` unit tests `test_laplacian_sign_convention` and `test_csr_diagonal_last`.

---

### §12.6 — Order-2 Chernoff for graph heat via Taylor truncation (NORMATIVE — Wave 2.1B)

**Setting.** Let `G = (V, E, w)` be a finite weighted graph with `N = |V|` nodes and graph Laplacian `L_G` as defined in §12.1. The graph PDE is

    u'(t) = −L_G u(t),    u(0) = u₀ ∈ ℝᴺ,    exact solution u(t) = e^{−t L_G} u₀.

**Reduction from §9.2.3.B.** For a constant coefficient field `a ≡ 1` on any graph, the ζ-A correction of §9.2.3.B reduces to zero: `a' = a'' = 0` implies `ζ_A(τ) = 0`, so the order-2 semigroup step becomes a pure Taylor-2 truncation:

    S₂(τ) = I − τ L_G + (τ²/2) L_G²

**Chernoff hypothesis check.**
- S₂(0) = I (identity at τ = 0). ✓
- S₂'(τ)|_{τ=0} = −L_G (generator recovered at leading order). ✓
- Quasi-contractivity: `‖S₂(τ)‖ ≤ 1 + O(τ²)` for τ small and L_G positive-semidefinite;
  see Chernoff (1968) Theorem 1 condition and Engel-Nagel (2000) §II.5 Remark 5.9.
  The L_G positive-semidefinite property holds for any weighted graph with non-negative weights
  (no negative-weight edges in semiflow-core).

**Convergence rate (Theorem 6 instantiated for graph heat).** Under Theorem 6 (§9.1), `n` steps of S₂(t/n) converge to `e^{−t L_G}`:

    ‖S₂(t/n)ⁿ u₀ − e^{−t L_G} u₀‖ = O(1/n²)    as n → ∞.

The constant hidden in O(1/n²) depends on `‖L_G³ u₀‖` and `t³`. The leading residual is:

    S₂(τ) u₀ − e^{−τ L_G} u₀ = +(τ³/6) L_G³ u₀ + O(τ⁴)

where the sign is positive because `S₂(τ) − exp(−τL_G) = [I−τL+τ²L²/2] − [I−τL+τ²L²/2−τ³L³/6+…] = +τ³L³/6 + …`.

**Gate T12_zeta_tau2_residual (NORMATIVE).** Exact sympy verification on P₅:
- Script: `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v2_1_zeta_tau2_residual.py`
- Claim verified: τ³ coefficient of `[S₂(τ)f − exp(−τL_G)f − (τ³/6)L_G³f]` = 0 per component.
- Status: PASS (2026-05-20).

**Variable a deferred.** Extension to `a: Fn(F) → F` requires non-trivial ζ-A (§9.2.3.B) and is outside the scope of this section. See §12.3 (DiffusionChernoff) for the 1D variable-a order-2 path.

**Implementation.** `GraphHeatChernoff::with_zeta_a(graph)` and `GraphHeatChernoff::from_owned_with_zeta_a(graph)` in `src/graph_heat.rs`. Zero-alloc steady-state invariant (R4) preserved via `ScratchPool::borrow_vec`.

---

### §12.7 — Order-4 Chernoff for graph heat via degree-4 Taylor truncation (NORMATIVE — Wave 2.1B)

**Setting.** Same as §12.6. The order-4 truncation is:

    S₄(τ) = Σ_{k=0}^{4} (−τ L_G)^k / k!
           = I − τ L_G + (τ²/2) L_G² − (τ³/6) L_G³ + (τ⁴/24) L_G⁴

**Cost.** Four SpMVs per step (L_G applied four times), compared to two SpMVs for S₂(τ). On graphs with N nodes and E edges, each SpMV costs O(N + E).

**Chernoff hypothesis check.** Same structure as §12.6 with higher matching order:
- S₄(0) = I. ✓
- S₄'(τ)|_{τ=0} = −L_G. ✓
- Quasi-contractivity for small τ and positive-semidefinite L_G holds by spectral argument:
  on the spectral range `λ ∈ [0, λ_max(L_G)]`, the polynomial `Σ_{k=0}^4 (−λτ)^k/k!` stays in (−1, 1]
  provided `τ λ_max ≤ r₄` where `r₄ ≈ 6.0` is the root of the truncated exponential polynomial of degree 4.
  This is more restrictive than for S₂(τ) (r₂ ≈ 2.0 is tighter, but the step count compensates).
  Practical CFL guidance: `τ ≤ 1/λ_max(L_G)` is conservative and safe for both S₂ and S₄.

**Convergence rate.** Under Theorem 6, `n` steps of S₄(t/n) converge to `e^{−t L_G}`:

    ‖S₄(t/n)ⁿ u₀ − e^{−t L_G} u₀‖ = O(1/n⁴)    as n → ∞.

The leading residual is:

    S₄(τ) u₀ − e^{−τ L_G} u₀ = +(τ⁵/120) L_G⁵ u₀ + O(τ⁶)

**Gate T12_zeta_tau4_residual (NORMATIVE).** Exact sympy verification on P₅:
