- Script: `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v2_1_zeta_tau4_residual.py`
- Claim verified: τ⁵ coefficient of `[S₄(τ)f − exp(−τL_G)f − (τ⁵/120)L_G⁵f]` = 0 per component.
- Status: PASS (2026-05-20).

**Comparison with Diffusion4thChernoff (§9.3).** The 1D finite-difference fourth-order kernel (§9.3, ADR-0005) achieves order-4 spatial accuracy via a cubic-Hermite stencil, then uses operator splitting for time. `GraphHeat4thChernoff` achieves order-4 temporal accuracy via the degree-4 Taylor polynomial; there is no spatial discretization (the graph structure is exact). The two approaches are complementary.

**References.** Higham (2008) §10 (polynomial approximations to matrix functions); Hochbruck-Ostermann (2010) §3 (Taylor-based exponential integrators for stiff problems).

**Implementation.** `GraphHeat4thChernoff<F>` in `src/graph_heat4.rs`. The ping-pong scratch pair uses `ScratchPool::take_vec` / `return_vec` to hold two simultaneous vectors without heap allocation per step (R4 invariant preserved).

---

### §12.8 — Strang split for bipartite graph Laplacian decompositions (NORMATIVE — Wave 2.1B)

**Setting.** Let `L_G = L_A + L_B` be a decomposition of the graph Laplacian into two sub-Laplacians `L_A` and `L_B`, both positive-semidefinite. The Strang (palindromic) product with order-2 sub-kernels S₂(t, L) = I − tL + (t²/2)L² is:

    P(τ) = S₂(τ/2, L_A) · S₂(τ, L_B) · S₂(τ/2, L_A)

**Order-2 global convergence of P(τ).** The palindromic composition `P(t/n)ⁿ → e^{−t L_G}` at global rate O(1/n²), regardless of whether `[L_A, L_B] = 0`.

*Proof sketch.* The local error expansion of P(τ) near τ = 0 satisfies (Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 §III.5 Theorem 5.1):

    P(τ) f − e^{−τ L_G} f = O(τ³)

i.e., the τ⁰, τ¹, and τ² coefficients of the residual vanish identically. This follows from:
1. The palindromic symmetry of the composition (L_A/2 — L_B — L_A/2) which cancels the first-order Baker-Campbell-Hausdorff commutator term.
2. The use of order-2 sub-kernels (S₂ rather than S₁ = I − tL), which ensures each leg matches e^{−tL} through τ² — cancelling the second cross term in the BCH expansion.

With order-1 sub-kernels, the palindromic product only achieves O(τ²) local error (the τ² coefficient is non-zero due to incomplete BCH cancellation). This is the mathematical reason why `new_bipartite_path` and `new_bipartite_cycle` use `with_zeta_a` (order-2) sub-kernels rather than `new` (order-1).

**Gate T12_strang_commuting_path_exact (NORMATIVE).** Exact sympy verification on P₅ (path graph, 5 nodes):
- Decomposition: L_A = edges {(0,1),(2,3)}, L_B = edges {(1,2),(3,4)} (bipartite edge-split by parity).
- Script: `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v2_1_strang_commuting_path.py`
- Claim verified: τ⁰, τ¹, τ² coefficients of `[P(τ)f − exp(−τL_G)f]` = 0 per component for test vector f = [1,2,3,4,5].
- Status: PASS (2026-05-20).

*Note on the Rust commutativity test.* The Rust test `bipartite_path_split_commutes_numerically` uses the all-ones vector `f = 1`, which lies in the kernel of every graph Laplacian (`L·1 = 0`). This means the commutator `[L_A, L_B]·1 = L_A L_B 1 − L_B L_A 1 = 0 − 0 = 0` trivially for any decomposition. On general vectors, `L_A` and `L_B` from the bipartite edge-split of P₅ do **not** commute (the commutator matrix has non-zero entries). The order-2 global convergence of `StrangSplitGraph` does not require `[L_A, L_B] = 0`; it follows from the palindromic symmetry argument above.

**Bipartite edge-split construction.** `split_laplacians_by_edge` in `src/strang_graph.rs` assigns edges with CSR traversal order index `k` (using `u < v` canonical form) to L_A (k even) or L_B (k odd). The split is constructive (no graph-colouring solver required) and deterministic. For bipartite graphs where the natural 2-colouring exists, the edge-parity split coincides with the bipartite partition.

**Safe constructors.** `StrangSplitGraph::new_bipartite_path(graph)` and `StrangSplitGraph::new_bipartite_cycle(graph)` construct the split using `GraphHeatChernoff::with_zeta_a` (order-2) sub-kernels. Passing `GraphHeatChernoff::new` (order-1) sub-kernels via the generic `StrangSplitGraph::new_generic(a, b)` constructor degrades global convergence to O(1/n). This is documented in the constructor-level rustdoc.

**Implementation.** `StrangSplitGraph<A, B, F>` in `src/strang_graph.rs`. The three-leg palindromic product allocates no temporary vectors beyond two ScratchPool buffers acquired via `take_graph_buf` / `return_graph_buf` (R4 invariant preserved).

**References.** Hairer, Lubich, Wanner (2006) §III.5 "Splitting methods" — §III.5 Theorem 5.1 (palindromic composition order). Chernoff (1968) Theorem 1. Engel-Nagel (2000) §II.5. Remizov (2025) Theorem 6.

---

### §12.9 — Magnus K=4 for time-dependent graph Laplacian `L_G(t)` (CITATION + NORMATIVE library policy — Wave 2.1C)

**Setting.** Let `G = (V, E, w(t))` be a graph with fixed `V`, fixed `E`, and time-varying edge weights `w(t): [0, T] → (0, ∞)^|E|` with `w ∈ C²([0, T])`. The Laplacian `L_G(t)` is defined per §12.1 with the time-varying weights. The PDE is

```text
∂_t u(t) = −L_G(t) u(t),   u(0) = u_0 ∈ ℝ^N.
```

**Exact solution.** `u(t) = exp(Ω(t)) u_0`, where `Ω(t)` is the Magnus expansion (Magnus 1954 *Commun. Pure Appl. Math.* **7**):

```text
Ω(τ) = ∫₀^τ A(s) ds − (1/2) ∫₀^τ ∫₀^s [A(s), A(u)] du ds + (nested commutators)
```

with `A(t) = −L_G(t)`. The series converges in operator norm whenever `∫₀^τ ‖A(s)‖₂ ds < π` (Blanes-Casas-Oteo-Ros 2009 *Phys. Rep.* **470** §3 Theorem 1). For bounded `L_G(·)` on finite graphs, this is `ρ̄_max · τ < π`; the library enforces a 50% safety margin `ρ̄_max · τ < π/2` (CITATION-derived NORMATIVE choice).

**Fourth-order Magnus method (CITATION).** The truncation `Ω₄(τ)`, evaluated by two-point Gauss-Legendre quadrature on `[0, τ]` with `c₁ = (3 − √3)/6`, `c₂ = (3 + √3)/6`, `b₁ = b₂ = 1/2`:

```text
A₁ := A(c₁ τ) = −L_G(c₁ τ),    A₂ := A(c₂ τ) = −L_G(c₂ τ)

Ω₄(τ) := (τ/2) (A₁ + A₂) + (√3 τ² / 12) [A₂, A₁]
```

satisfies `‖Ω(τ) − Ω₄(τ)‖₂ = O(τ⁵)` (Iserles+ 2000 *Acta Numerica* **9** §5.5 Theorem 5.2). This is the classical fourth-order Magnus method; no new theorem.

**Chernoff hypothesis check** (per §12.2 hypotheses; verified for `S₄(τ) := exp(Ω₄(τ))`):

- `S₄(0) = exp(0) = I` ✓
- `S₄'(0) = (d/dτ) exp(Ω₄(τ))|_{τ=0} = (d/dτ) Ω₄(τ)|_{τ=0} = (A₁ + A₂)/2|_{τ=0} = A(0) = −L_G(0)` ✓
  (Closability is automatic: `−L_G(0)` is bounded on `ℝ^N`.)
- Quasi-contractivity: `‖exp(Ω₄(τ))‖₂ ≤ exp(τ · ρ̄_max)` → `(M, ω) = (1, ρ̄_max)` ✓

By §12.2 (Chernoff product formula) and Iserles+ 2000 §5.5 Theorem 5.2:

```text
‖(S₄(t/n))^n u_0 − u_exact(t)‖₂ = O(1/n⁴)   for any u_0 ∈ ℝ^N.
```

**Library policy (NORMATIVE).** `semiflow-core` ships `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff<F>` (`src/magnus_graph.rs`) implementing this method. The contract `LaplacianAtTime<F> = Box<dyn Fn(F) -> Arc<Laplacian<F>>>` requires:

1. `lap_at_t` is **pure** — same `t` returns equal output.
2. **Topology fixed** — `Laplacian::row_ptr` and `Laplacian::col_idx` returned by `lap_at_t(t)` MUST equal those of the topology graph passed to the constructor, for all `t ∈ [0, T]`. Only `Laplacian::vals` may vary in `t`.
3. **Smoothness** — `lap_at_t(·)` MUST be twice continuously differentiable in `t` (required by GL4 quadrature error analysis; caller responsibility).

**Out of scope (v2.1).** Variable topology (`row_ptr`/`col_idx` change in `t`), time-discontinuous `L_G(t)`, order-6 Magnus, self-adjoint variants for unitary Schrödinger semigroup. Deferred to v2.2+.

**Convergence-radius check (NORMATIVE library behaviour).** Each `apply_into` call validates `ρ̄_max · τ < π/2` and returns `SemiflowError::OutOfMagnusRadius` on violation, where `ρ̄_max` is the caller-supplied peak Gershgorin bound. Caller is responsible for supplying a tight bound; the library does not search the time axis.

**Acceptance gate (G11).** Time-dependent path graph `P_64`, `w(t) = 1 + 0.3·sin(πt)`, `t_final = 0.5`, self-convergence at 2× refinement. OLS slope on `(log n_steps, log sup_err_self)` over `n_steps ∈ {10, 20, 40, 80, 160}` (f64) and `{2, 3, 4, 6, 8}` (f32, lower 3 points). Threshold: slope ≤ −3.95 (f64), ≤ −3.50 (f32) per ADR-0051.

**Sympy gate (T12_magnus_consistency).** `.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v2_1c_magnus_consistency.py` re-derives the GL4 abscissae from `(3 ± √3)/6`, verifies the `√3/12` commutator coefficient, and confirms `Ω₄` matches `Ω` through `τ⁴` on a `P_4` path Laplacian with `w(t) = 1 + 0.3·sin(πt)`. Status: PASS (2026-05-20).

**References.**
- W. Magnus, *Commun. Pure Appl. Math.* **7** (1954) 649–673.
- A. Iserles, H. Z. Munthe-Kaas, S. P. Nørsett, A. Zanna, *Acta Numerica* **9** (2000) 215–365.
- S. Blanes, F. Casas, J. A. Oteo, J. Ros, *Physics Reports* **470** (2009) 151–238.
- M. Hochbruck, A. Ostermann, *Acta Numerica* **19** (2010) 209–286.
- I. D. Remizov, *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* **27**(4) (2025) — Theorem 6.

---

## 8. References

1. I. D. Remizov, *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* **27**(4) (2025). DOI 10.46698/a3908-1212-5385-q. arXiv:2301.06765.
2. P. R. Chernoff, *J. Funct. Anal.* **2** (1968) 238–242. DOI 10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7.
3. O. E. Galkin, I. D. Remizov, *Israel J. Math.* **265** (2025) 929–943. DOI 10.1007/s11856-024-2678-x.
4. E. Hairer, C. Lubich, G. Wanner, *Geometric Numerical Integration* (2nd ed., Springer 2006). §III.5 "Splitting methods" — canonical reference for the Strang order-2 result and palindromic-composition theorem (§9 here).
5. `.dev-docs/research/literature-validation.md` — verbatim PDF extraction and numerical sanity checks.

## §13 — Storage refactors for v0.13.0 (NORMATIVE)

The v0.13.0 perf wave introduces three internal storage refactors that **preserve all theorem invariants** (Theorem 6 Chernoff convergence, Theorem 7' tensor-product τ²-order):

1. **Strang3D serial scratch** (ADR-0022 Amendment 1): pre-allocated `y_scratch`, `z_scratch` of length N³, reused across Strang steps. Allocation timing change only; arithmetic per node unchanged. Bit-equal regression gate `STRANG3D_SERIAL_SCRATCH_BIT_EQUAL` enforces byte-identity vs pre-refactor scalar output.

2. **HalfNodeCoeffCache for TruncatedExp4** (ADR-0034 Amendment 1): caller's `a: impl Fn(F)→F` is evaluated at half-node points (x_i ± dx/2, x_i ± 3·dx/2) **once at constructor time**, stored as `a_at_halfnodes: Vec<F>` of length 2N. Hot loop indexes the Vec instead of calling the closure. Mathematically equivalent IFF `a(x)` is pure (deterministic, no side effects) — a contract already required by ADR-0034.

3. **TruncatedExp4 SIMD path** (ADR-0019 Amendment 2): 5-point K-kernel stencil and K=4 Horner accumulation evaluated via AVX2/NEON intrinsics with FMA-disabled (`-C target-feature=-fma` build flag). Arithmetic operation order preserved bit-for-bit vs scalar path (cite SLEEF arXiv 2001.09258 for technique; Compensated Horner arXiv cs/0610122 for theoretical bound preservation). Bit-equality gate `TEXP4_SIMD_BIT_EQUAL`.

These are **STORAGE-ONLY** refactors: per-node arithmetic, error bounds, CFL constraints, and operator-splitting symmetry remain identical to v0.12.0. No DEVIATION introduced (see `docs/audit-findings-v0_13_0.md`).

**Algorithmic floor note** (per ADR-0037): even after Wave B fully ships, RC TruncatedExp4 remains ~15-20× slower than KIOPS Krylov-Magnus on bench F2 (Gaudreault et al. 2018, J. Comput. Phys. 372:236-255). This is **deliberate**: Krylov-Arnoldi requires implicit Hessenberg assembly which violates RC's "explicit by design" principle (ROADMAP.md:354). RC retains H-MEM Pareto dominance (125× less memory than kiops on F2).

---

## §14 — Variable-topology graph Laplacian `L_G(t)` (NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

This section extends §12 (graph PDE) to **piecewise-smooth time-varying generators**. It introduces **no new mathematics** — every formula is either a direct restatement of §12 within a smooth time segment, or a citation of established splitting-method theory at segment boundaries. The library contribution is the `GraphTraj<F>` data structure (ADR-0052) and the segment-walking algorithm in `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff::evolve_with_traj` (ADR-0054).

### §14.1 — Piecewise-smooth trajectory `GraphTraj<F>` (NORMATIVE)

A **graph trajectory** on horizon `T > 0` is a tuple `(0 = t_0 < t_1 < … < t_K = T, G_0, G_1, …, G_{K−1}, w_0, w_1, …, w_{K−1})` where:

- `t_0, …, t_K` are the **breakpoints** (strictly increasing).
- For each segment `k ∈ {0, …, K−1}`, the graph `G_k = (V, E_k, w_k(·))` has a fixed vertex set `V` (independent of `k`), edge set `E_k`, and edge-weight function `w_k: [t_k, t_{k+1}] × E_k → (0, ∞)`.
- Within each segment, `w_k(·)` is `C²` in `t` (required by GL₄ quadrature error analysis; §12.9 ADR-0051).
- At a breakpoint `t_k`, the topology MAY change discretely: `E_{k-1} ≠ E_k` is permitted.

**Right-continuous convention.** At `t = t_k` for `k ≥ 1`, the Laplacian is sampled from segment `k` (i.e., `lap_at_t(t_k) = w_k(t_k) ∘ G_k`). This makes the trajectory single-valued at every `t ∈ [0, T]`.

**Library invariant** (CSR layout per segment). Within segment `k`, every `Laplacian` returned by `w_k(t)` MUST have `row_ptr` and `col_idx` equal to those of `G_k` (per §12.1 + ADR-0048 invariant I-immut). Only `vals` may vary in `t` within a segment.

**Resource bound** (NORMATIVE). `K ≤ 65_535` (constructor-enforced per ADR-0052). Reflects the practical limit of CSR-segment storage on modern hardware (~16 MB at K=65_535, average 1024-edge graphs).

### §14.2 — Variable-coefficient graph diffusion `L_a = A^{1/2} L_G A^{1/2}` (CITATION; ADR-0053)

For per-node conductivity `a: V → (0, ∞)`, define `A = diag(a(0), …, a(N−1))`. The **symmetric weighted Laplacian** is `L_a := A^{1/2} L_G A^{1/2}` (Belkin-Niyogi 2008 §3 — eq. (3.2)).

**Discrete ζ-A correction** (ADR-0053 Wave 2.2A). The τ²-truncation of `exp(−τ L_a)` is:

```math
S(τ) f = f − τ L_a f + (τ²/2) L_a² f + O(τ³)
```

**Order 2 for all positive `a`** (no regime envelope restriction). Verification gate T12N
confirms that the truncation `I − τL_a + (τ²/2)L_a²` has O(τ³) local error for all
variable `a` and `w` (`.dev-docs/verification/scripts/verify_v2_2_variable_a_graph_residual.py`).

**Correction note (v2.2.0)**: The original §14.2 draft included a `−(τ²/12) D_a^{(2)} f`
term (1D Stratonovich analogy). This term was found to be HARMFUL for the graph case:
since `L_a = A^{1/2} L_G A^{1/2}` is an exact linear operator, the plain Taylor truncation
`I − τL_a + (τ²/2)L_a²` already achieves O(τ³); adding `D_a^{(2)}` introduces a spurious
O(τ²) offset that degrades global convergence from order 2 to order 1 (G13 gate regression,
fixed in v2.2.0 release). The `D_a^{(2)}` formula is retained here for reference only:

```math
[D_a^{(2)} f]_i = ∑_{j ∈ N(i)} w(i, j) · (a(j) − a(i)) · (a(j)·f(j) − a(i)·f(i)) / (a(i) · a(j))
```

### §14.3 — Time-discontinuous `L_G(t)` via segment walking (CITATION + NORMATIVE; ADR-0054)

For a piecewise-smooth trajectory `(t_0, …, t_K)` (per §14.1), the exact solution of `u'(t) = −L_G(t) u(t)` is the product of segment-wise matrix exponentials:

```math
u(T) = U_K U_{K-1} ⋯ U_1 u(0),  where  U_k = exp(∫_{t_{k-1}}^{t_k} −L_G(s) ds)
```

Within each segment, the Magnus expansion (§12.9 + ADR-0051) gives `U_k ≈ exp(Ω₄^{(k)}(t_k − t_{k-1}))` accurate to order 4 in `τ_k := (t_k − t_{k-1}) / n_steps_per_segment`. The library implements this via `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff::evolve_with_traj` (ADR-0054):

```text
state ← f0
for k = 0..K-1:
    rebind self.lap_at_t ← traj.weight_fns[k]
    τ ← (t_{k+1} − t_k) / n_steps_per_segment
    for step = 0..n_steps_per_segment:
        state ← apply_into_at(t_k + step·τ, τ, state)
return state
```

Order 4 within each segment + order ∞ matrix-product at boundaries (no discretisation error from the segment join itself; the join is an exact operator composition).

**Convergence-radius check per segment** (NORMATIVE). For each segment `k`, the library validates `ρ̄_max^{(k)} · τ_k < π/2` and returns `SemiflowError::OutOfMagnusRadius` on violation. Caller MAY supply per-segment `ρ̄_max^{(k)}` via an extension API (deferred to v2.3+); v2.2 uses the trajectory-wide `rho_bar_max` from the `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff` constructor.

**Acceptance gates**:
- **G12** (slope, NORMATIVE): 3-segment toy on `P_64` with topology change + smooth edge weights, slope ≤ −3.95 (f64) per ADR-0052.
- **G14** (jump-resolution, NORMATIVE): star-graph S_4 with edge-weight switch at fixed breakpoints, demonstrates `evolve_with_traj` recovers order-4 while bare `apply_into_at` (no trajectory) collapses to order-1 — see ADR-0054.

### §14.4 — References

- F. R. K. Chung, *Spectral Graph Theory* (AMS 1997), §1.2 — weighted Laplacian.
- M. Belkin, P. Niyogi, *Found. Comp. Math.* **8** (2008) 7–37 — symmetric Laplacian conjugation.
- O. E. Galkin, I. D. Remizov, *Israel J. Math.* **265** (2025) 929–943 — discrete ζ-A correction.
- A. Iserles, H. Z. Munthe-Kaas, S. P. Nørsett, A. Zanna, *Acta Numerica* **9** (2000) §5 — Magnus method.
- E. Caglioti, M. Pulvirenti, F. Rousset, "Operator splitting for discontinuous generators" — segment-walking pattern.

---

## §15 — Adjoint-Chernoff backward semigroup (CITATION-only; library contribution = wrapper API)

This section establishes the mathematical foundation for the `AdjointChernoff<C, F>` wrapper (ADR-0055), which exposes the **dual semigroup** `S*(τ) = exp(τA*)` for any forward semigroup `S(τ) = exp(τA)` whose state space is a `HilbertState<F>`.

### §15.1 — Dual semigroup characterisation (CITATION)

For a strongly continuous semigroup `S(τ)` on a Hilbert space `H` with generator `A`, the **adjoint semigroup** `S*(τ)` is defined by

```math
⟨S(τ) f, g⟩ = ⟨f, S*(τ) g⟩    for all f, g ∈ H
```

(Pazy 1983 *Semigroups of Linear Operators*, §1.10 Theorem 10.4). For *self-adjoint* `A` (i.e., `A = A*`), the duality is trivial: `S*(τ) = S(τ)`.

For *non-self-adjoint* `A = A_sym + B` where `A_sym` is self-adjoint and `B` is a bounded perturbation, the true adjoint is `S*(τ) = exp(τ A*)`. For `A = −Δ + b·∂_x` (constant `b`), the L²-adjoint is `A* = −Δ − b·∂_x` and `S*(τ) = exp(τ(−Δ − b·∂_x))` — the same characteristic-flow kernel with drift sign negated. For variable `b(x)`, the L²-formal adjoint also includes a `−b'(x)` reaction term; the characteristic-flow kernel with negated `b` is exact only for constant `b`.

**NORMATIVE NOTE (ADR-0114, 2026-05-31)**: The Engel-Nagel bounded-perturbation expansion `S*(τ) = exp(τ A_sym) − τ · proj_B + O(τ²)` where `proj_B` is the orthogonal projection onto `closure(range(B))` is under-specified for discrete drift operators. In particular, `proj_B` is NOT computable from `apply_into`+`dot`+`axpy` alone (no access to `Bᵀ`), and any generator-independent scalar correction of the form `dst += −τ·(‖src‖²/n)·src` is provably WRONG (violates the adjoint identity by up to ~96% for large drift). The correct implementation requires a transpose-apply primitive `apply_adjoint_into` on the inner type (see `AdjointApply<F>` trait, ADR-0114).

### §15.1.bis — Order-preservation rule (NORMATIVE library; ADR-0055/ADR-0114)

The `AdjointChernoff<C, F>::order()` returns

```text
order() = inner.order()                if self_adjoint
        = min(inner.order(), 2)        otherwise
```

**Rationale**: for the non-self-adjoint path, the `apply_adjoint_into` method provides an order-2 approximation to `exp(τ Aᵀ)` for supported inners (`DriftReactionChernoff`). Even if `inner.order() == 4`, the wrapper's overall order is 2 due to the discrete approximation of the transpose. For self-adjoint inners, the wrapper is a no-op (just delegates to `inner.apply_into`).

### §15.2 — References

- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to PDEs* (Springer 1983), §1.10.
- K.-J. Engel, R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations* (Springer 2000), §I.5, §II.4.
- M. Hochbruck, A. Ostermann, *Acta Numerica* **19** (2010) §3.

---

## §16 — Order-6 Magnus expansion (CITATION; library contribution = `MagnusGraphHeat6thChernoff`)

This section extends §12.9 (Magnus K=4 on graphs, ADR-0051) to **order 6** via three-point Gauss-Legendre quadrature (GL₆) and the canonical Blanes-Casas-Oteo-Ros (BCOR) 2-commutator form. No new theorems; direct citation of Blanes+ 2009 *Phys. Rep.* §4 / Table 5 and Iserles+ 2000 *Acta Numerica* §6.

**Note (ADR-0114)**: An earlier version of this section stated a 4-commutator Ω₆ formula with remainder `O(τ⁵)` attributed to "Blanes+ 2009 Table 6, Method M₆[2,1]". That formula achieved only global order ~2 on non-commuting `L(t)` (independently measured local slope ~3 by scipy/DOP853 on a 3×3 non-commuting family). It was WRONG. The corrected BCOR-6 2-commutator form below is the formula that BCOR Table 5 actually publishes; it achieves local truncation error O(τ⁷) (global order 6), independently verified (see fix-spec A.5, numeric confirmation local slope ≈7.1 on non-commuting ℝ³ family).

### §16.1 — Three-point Gauss-Legendre quadrature (CITATION)

The classical GL₆ rule on `[0, 1]` has abscissae and weights

```math
c₁ = (5 − √15) / 10,    c₂ = 1 / 2,    c₃ = (5 + √15) / 10
b₁ = 5/18,              b₂ = 8/18,     b₃ = 5/18
```

(Stroud-Secrest 1966 Table 9.1; reproduced in Iserles+ 2000 Table III). The quadrature error on `C^k` data is `O(τ^{2k+1})` for `k ≤ 6` — sufficient for order-6 Magnus on `C³` data.

### §16.2 — Order-6 Magnus operator Ω₆(τ) — BCOR-6 2-commutator form (NORMATIVE; ADR-0114)

Sample `A_i = A(c_i · τ) = −L_G(c_i · τ)` at the three GL₆ abscissae. Define scaled GL₆ generators:

```math
B₁ = τ · A₂
B₂ = τ · (√15 / 3) · (A₃ − A₁)
B₃ = τ · (10 / 3)  · (A₃ − 2·A₂ + A₁)
```

Then the first two commutator intermediates:

```math
C₁ = [B₁, B₂]
C₂ = −(1/60) · [B₁, 2·B₃ + C₁]
```

And the order-6 Magnus operator:

```math
Ω₆(τ) = B₁ + (1/12)·B₃ + (1/240)·[−20·B₁ − B₃ + C₁ , B₂ + C₂]
```

Local truncation error: **O(τ⁷)**. Global order: **6** on non-commuting `A(t)`.

This is the canonical form from Blanes-Casas-Oteo-Ros *Phys. Rep.* **470** (2009) §4, method with 2 commutator evaluations. It uses only **2 commutator evaluations** (`C₁`, then `C₂` and the outer bracket), cheaper than the previously incorrect 4-commutator form.

**Cost**: 3 SpMV for `A_i v`, ~8 SpMV for the 2 commutator evaluations, + 22 ScratchPool buffers for the degree-6 Taylor of `exp(Ω₆) v` ≈ 18 sparse mat-vec per Taylor term.

### §16.3 — Convergence radius (CITATION)

The matrix-Magnus convergence radius `∫₀^τ ‖A(s)‖₂ ds < π` (Blanes+ 2009 Theorem 1) is order-independent. The library uses the same 50% safety margin `ρ̄_max · τ < π/2` as ADR-0051 — see §12.9.

### §16.4 — Acceptance gate (G17′ + T14N, ADR-0114)

- **G17′ slope gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0056, ADR-0114): path graph `P_64` with **distinct per-edge phases** `wᵢ(t) = 1 + 0.3·sin(π·(t + φᵢ))` where `φᵢ = (i · 0.13) mod 1` (non-commuting family, `[L(t₁),L(t₂)] ≠ 0` on general ICs). IC: `f_i = sin(0.31πi/N) + 0.2·cos(1.7i)` (not all-ones — avoids ker L trap). The test includes a **non-commutativity precondition assertion** `‖[L(t₁),L(t₂)]·f‖ > 1e-6` that fails loudly if the family is accidentally made commuting again. `t_final = 0.5`, `n_steps ∈ {5, 10, 20, 40, 80}`. Slope ≤ −5.85 (f64). **f32 NOT GATED** — `MagnusGraphHeat6thChernoff` does not implement `ChernoffFunction<f32>` (compile-time gated).
- **T14N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0056, ADR-0114): verify that `U(τ) − exp(Ω₆_BCOR(τ)) = O(τ⁷)` symbolically on a non-commuting 4×4 phased-path family (NOT line-by-line against the old wrong coefficient table).

### §16.5 — References

- A. H. Stroud, D. Secrest, *Gaussian Quadrature Formulas* (Prentice-Hall 1966), Table 9.1.
- A. Iserles, H. Z. Munthe-Kaas, S. P. Nørsett, A. Zanna, *Acta Numerica* **9** (2000) §6, Table III.
- S. Blanes, F. Casas, J. A. Oteo, J. Ros, *Phys. Rep.* **470** (2009) §4, Table 5 — canonical 2-commutator order-6 Magnus method (BCOR-6).
- Fix-spec: `.dev-docs/reports/bug-a-b-coremath-fixspec-2026-05-31.md` §A.1–A.8 (FORMULA_WRONG + CODE_BUG + TEST_MASK analysis, independent numeric proofs).

---

## §17 — Schrödinger unitary semigroup (real-only `Δ + V` scope; CITATION + NORMATIVE scope policy)

This section establishes the foundation for `SchrodingerChernoff<F>` (ADR-0057) — the first **unitary group** in `semiflow-core`. Scope is constrained to `i·∂_t ψ = (−Δ + V(x)) ψ` with real potential `V: ℝ^N → ℝ` and the state `ψ` represented as `(ψ_re, ψ_im) ∈ ℝ^N × ℝ^N`. Complex-valued generalisation (full `SemiflowComplex` trait) is deferred to v2.3+ per ADR-0057 §"Out of scope".

### §17.1 — Strongly continuous unitary group (CITATION)

For self-adjoint Hamiltonian `H = −Δ + V(x)` on `L²(ℝ)` with `V ∈ L^∞`, Stone's theorem (Engel-Nagel 2000 §IV.6 Theorem 6.5) gives a strongly continuous unitary group `U(t) = exp(−i t H)` satisfying

```math
U(t) U(t)* = U(t)* U(t) = I    for all t ∈ ℝ
‖U(t) ψ‖₂ = ‖ψ‖₂               (norm conservation)
```

The group is generated by `−i H` (anti-self-adjoint).

### §17.2 — Real representation via `(ψ_re, ψ_im)` decomposition (NORMATIVE library; ADR-0057)

Write `ψ = ψ_re + i ψ_im` with `ψ_re, ψ_im ∈ ℝ^N`. Substituting into `i ψ_t = H ψ` gives

```math
∂_t ψ_re = + H ψ_im
∂_t ψ_im = − H ψ_re
```

This is a 2N-dim real system with **skew-symmetric** generator

```math
G = ⎡  0       H ⎤
    ⎣ −H       0 ⎦
```

`G + G^T = 0` ⇒ `exp(τG)` is orthogonal ⇒ `(ψ_re, ψ_im) ↦ exp(τG)(ψ_re, ψ_im)` preserves the 2N-dim ℓ² norm = `‖ψ‖_{L²}^2`. Unitarity in the real representation = orthogonality.

### §17.3 — Strang splitting on `Δ + V` (CITATION + NORMATIVE; ADR-0057)

The library splits `G` into kinetic `T = ⎡0, K; -K, 0⎤` (with `K = −Δ` on the grid) and potential `V = ⎡0, V; -V, 0⎤` (with `V = diag(V(x_i))`). The Strang composition

```math
S(τ) = exp(τ V/2) · exp(τ T) · exp(τ V/2)
```

is **order 2 globally** (Sanz-Serna-Calvo 1994 §4.5 — palindromic composition). Per-step cost: 2 V-rotations + 1 kinetic step.

**V-rotation** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0057). For each node `i`, with `α := V(x_i) · τ`:

```math
⎡ψ_re_new[i]⎤   ⎡ cos α    sin α ⎤ ⎡ψ_re[i]⎤
⎢            ⎥ = ⎢                 ⎥ ⎢        ⎥
⎣ψ_im_new[i]⎦   ⎣−sin α    cos α ⎦ ⎣ψ_im[i]⎦
```

The 2×2 rotation matrix is exactly the real representation of multiplication by `exp(−i α)`. Determinant = `cos² α + sin² α = 1` (unitary).

**Kinetic step** (NORMATIVE — Amendment 1, 2026-05-21). The kinetic propagator `exp(iτΔ/(2m))` is approximated via the Crank-Nicolson (Cayley map) scheme; see §17.4 for the normative specification.

### §17.4 — Kinetic step via Crank-Nicolson (Cayley map) (NORMATIVE)

The kinetic propagator `exp(iτΔ/(2m))` is approximated by the Cayley map
(Crank-Nicolson):

```math
K_CN(τ) = (I − iτΔ/(4m))⁻¹ · (I + iτΔ/(4m))
```

This Möbius transformation maps the imaginary axis to the unit circle, so
`‖K_CN(τ)‖_2 = 1` exactly. In real-only representation `(ψ_re, ψ_im)`:

```math
K_CN(τ) ⎡ψ_re⎤ = (I + A²)⁻¹ · ⎡ I    −A ⎤ · ⎡ψ_re⎤
         ⎣ψ_im⎦                  ⎣ A     I ⎦   ⎣ψ_im⎦
```

where `A = τΔ/(4m)` and `(I + A²)` is solved by banded LU per step.

Mixed-precision strategy: all arithmetic in f64 regardless of public-API `F`
type. This ensures the cross-binding sup-error identity (≤3 ULP per ADR-0059)
holds for f32 users without sacrificing unitarity tolerance.

**Implementation**: `cn_kinetic_step_f64` in `src/schrodinger.rs` solves the
block system via `pentadiag_solve_f64` (band-5 LU). 12 f64 working buffers are
pre-allocated in `SchrodingerChernoff::new()` and reused per step (R4 zero-alloc,
gated by `tests/schrodinger_zero_alloc.rs`).

Reference: Iserles 2009 §8, "A First Course in the Numerical Analysis of
Differential Equations", Cayley map for unitary group SU(N).

### §17.5 — Acceptance gates (G18 + G19 + T15N)

- **G18 unitarity gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0057): Gaussian wavepacket on `[-5, 5]`, N=64, `V(x) = ½ x²` (harmonic oscillator), `t_final = 1.0`, `n_steps = 100`. `|‖ψ(t_final)‖² − ‖ψ_0‖²| < 1e-12` (f64) / `< 1e-6` (f32). Slope ≤ −1.95 (f64) / ≤ −1.50 (f32) on n_steps refinement.
- **G19 harmonic-oscillator oracle gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0057): Gaussian centred at `x=1`, σ=0.5. After period `T = 2π`, `‖ψ(T) − e^{i·ϕ} ψ_0‖_2 < 1e-3` for some real phase ϕ.
- **T15N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0057): verify the V-rotation 2×2 matrix on symbolic `α` is exactly `[[cos α, sin α], [-sin α, cos α]]` and that its determinant is 1.

### §17.6 — References

- K.-J. Engel, R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations* (Springer 2000), §IV.6.
- J. M. Sanz-Serna, M. P. Calvo, *Numerical Hamiltonian Problems* (Chapman & Hall 1994), §4.5.
- S. Blanes, F. Casas, A. Murua, *J. Chem. Phys.* **124** (2006) 234105.
- A. Iserles, *A First Course in the Numerical Analysis of Differential Equations* (Cambridge 2009), §8 — Cayley map for unitary group SU(N).

---

## §18 — Generic non-separable mixed operators `NonSeparableMixedChernoff<X, Y, F, S>` (NORMATIVE refactor pointer; ADR-0058)

This section is an API refactor pointer. The mathematical content for non-separable 2D operators is fully covered in §10.7 (constant-c case, v0.7.0) and §10.7-ter (anisotropic `β(x,y)` case, v0.9.0). v2.2 ADR-0058 unifies the two v0.7.0 + v0.9.0 implementations under a single generic `NonSeparableMixedChernoff<X, Y, F, S>` parameterised by the state type `S`. The existing types `NonSeparable2DChernoff` and `NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff` become type aliases.

**No math change**. The Strang-style palindromic 5-leg composition (Theorem 7-bis, §10.7-ter) is unchanged. The order-2 in τ result (Theorem 7-bis Corollary) applies to both `MixedDerivOperator::ScalarCoupling` and `MixedDerivOperator::BetaCoupling` impls — only the discretisation of the mixed-Taylor coupling step changes between them (one scalar multiply vs one per-node lookup).

**Library policy** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0058):

- Both `NonSeparable2DChernoff` and `NonSeparable2DAnisotropicChernoff` are PUBLIC `pub type` aliases. Removal would be a MAJOR break.
- New code MAY use `NonSeparableMixedChernoff::with_scalar_c` or `with_beta` for explicit intent.
- ADR-0033 (deprecation policy) is SUPERSEDED — neither type is deprecated.

**Forward compatibility note**: v2.3+ may introduce graph-mixed extensions (e.g., `NonSeparableMixedGraphChernoff` over `S = GraphSignal<F>`) — the generic abstraction already supports this once `GraphSignal<F>` implements the necessary 2-axis structure (currently does not in v2.2 scope).

**No new sympy gate**. The existing §10.7-ter T7N + T7N_NS2D_aniso gates re-pass byte-identical via the type-aliased call paths. G20 alias-identity gate (ADR-0058) verifies bit-equality at the API surface.

---

## §19 — Order-6 spatial graph diffusion (`GraphHeat6thChernoff`; NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

This section extends §12.7 (order-4 spatial, `GraphHeat4thChernoff`) to **order 6** on static weighted graphs. No new theorems; direct citation of Higham 2008 *Functions of Matrices* §10 (Taylor methods for `exp(A)`) and Hochbruck-Ostermann 2010 *Acta Numerica* §3 (truncated-exponential families on bounded operators). See ADR-0062.

### §19.1 — Truncated operator-Taylor (NORMATIVE definition)

The order-6 Chernoff approximant for the static graph heat semigroup is

```math
S_6(τ) f = Σ_{k=0}^{6} (−τ L_G)^k / k! · f
        = f − τ L_G f + (τ²/2) L_G² f − (τ³/6) L_G³ f
          + (τ⁴/24) L_G⁴ f − (τ⁵/120) L_G⁵ f + (τ⁶/720) L_G⁶ f.
```

This defines `GraphHeat6thChernoff<F: SemiflowFloat>::apply_into` in `crates/semiflow-core/src/graph_heat6.rs`. Two ping-pong scratch buffers (`ScratchPool::take_vec`/`return_vec`) carry the SpMV intermediates `L_G^k · src` for `k ∈ {1, …, 6}`; zero heap allocation in steady state.

### §19.2 — Order verification (CITATION)

Higham 2008 §10 establishes that for bounded `A` (matrix on `ℝ^N`), the truncated Taylor series satisfies

```math
‖exp(τA) − Σ_{k=0}^{K} (τA)^k / k!‖_2  ≤  (‖τA‖^{K+1} / (K+1)!) · exp(‖τA‖).
```

For `A = −L_G` (real symmetric PSD), `‖A‖_2 = λ_max(L_G) ≤ 2 · max_i deg_w(i)` (Gershgorin; §12.1). Therefore at `K = 6`,

```math
‖exp(−τL_G) − S_6(τ)‖_2  ≤  (τ · λ_max)^7 / 5040 · exp(τ · λ_max)  =  O(τ⁷),
```

so `S_6(τ) f = exp(−τL_G) f + O(τ⁷)`, satisfying the Chernoff hypothesis `S(τ) = I + τA + O(τ²)` with order ≥ 2 trivially and matching the matrix exponential through `τ⁶`. Convergence `(S_6(t/n))^n f → exp(−tL_G) f` proceeds via §12.2 (Pazy 1983 §1.3 Theorem 1.3 bounded case) at rate `O(n⁻⁶)` on `f ∈ D(A^7) = ℝ^N`.

### §19.3 — Stability domain (NORMATIVE bound)

The degree-6 Taylor of `e^z` on the negative real axis has roots in the complex plane; for spectral safety we require `τ · λ_max(L_G) < 6` (twice the radius of monotonic convergence of `Σ z^k/k!` on negative reals, Hochbruck-Ostermann 2010 §3 Table 2). The library validates this via the existing `SemiflowError::DomainViolation` path when `τ < 0` or `τ` not finite; **the spectral bound is the caller's responsibility** (matching `GraphHeat4thChernoff` policy — graph kernels expose `spectral_radius_bound()` for caller-side scheduling).

### §19.4 — Precision policy (NORMATIVE — ADR-0062)

`GraphHeat6thChernoff<F: SemiflowFloat>` is generic over `F` (f32 AND f64). The type signature carries no commutator coefficient `τ^k · √15 / 1080` (which is what forced ADR-0056 Magnus K=6 to be f64-only). The only non-trivial small coefficient is the τ⁶/720 Taylor term, which is benign in f32 arithmetic. However: on a smooth initial condition like `cos(2π i/N)` the dominant excited mode has eigenvalue `λ ≈ 4 sin²(π/N) ≈ 4π²/N²`, so the order-6 truncation residual `(τλ)⁷/5040` sits below f32 ε ≈ 1.2e-7. **f32 slope on smooth IC is therefore not gated**; an **absolute-floor gate** at `|err|_∞ ≤ 5 × 10⁻⁶` after 12 steps verifies numerical correctness without depending on a measurable slope.

### §19.5 — Acceptance gates (G21 + T16N)

- **G21 f64 slope gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0062): static `P_64`, smooth IC `f_i = cos(2π i / N)`, `t_final = 1.0`, `n_steps ∈ {5, 8, 12}` (last point at clean order-6 floor ~5e-13). Slope threshold: ≤ −5.85.
- **G21 f32 absolute-floor gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0062): same workload, `n_steps = 12`. Threshold: `|err|_∞ ≤ 5 × 10⁻⁶`. f32 slope NOT gated; see §19.4.
- **T16N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0062): on a symbolic 4×4 path Laplacian, verify `S_6(τ) f − exp(−τL_G) f = O(τ⁷)` by sympy series expansion. Pure symbolic; no library runtime.

### §19.6 — References

- N. J. Higham, *Functions of Matrices: Theory and Computation* (SIAM 2008), §10 — Taylor methods for `exp(A)`.
- M. Hochbruck, A. Ostermann, *Acta Numerica* **19** (2010) §3 — truncated-exponential families on bounded operators.
- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators*, Springer 1983, §1.3.

---

## §20 — Variable-coefficient time-dependent graph Magnus K=4 (`VarCoefMagnusGraphHeatChernoff`; NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

This section composes the variable-coefficient graph operator `L_a(t) = A(t)^{1/2} L_G(t) A(t)^{1/2}` of §12.7 (constant-time variant) with the order-4 Magnus expansion of §12.9 (constant-coefficient time-dependent variant). The mathematical content is the union of those two CITATIONs; the library contribution is the closure-driven sampling of **both** `a(t)` and `L_G(t)` at GL₂ abscissae. See ADR-0063.

### §20.1 — Operator definition (NORMATIVE)

Let `t ↦ Arc<Laplacian<F>>` be the `LaplacianAtTime<F>` closure (§14.1) and let `t ↦ Vec<F>` (length `N`, all entries strictly positive and finite) be a `WeightAtTime<F>` closure. The variable-coefficient time-dependent graph operator is

```math
L_a(t) : ℝ^N → ℝ^N,    [L_a(t) v]_i = sqrt(a_i(t)) · [L_G(t) (sqrt(a(t)) ⊙ v)]_i.
```

This is exactly the operator-form `apply_la_on_slice` (`crates/semiflow-core/src/graph_var_coef.rs:208`) with the diagonal `sqrt(a(t))` and the Laplacian `L_G(t)` both sampled at time `t`. `L_a(t)` is symmetric positive semidefinite for every `t` (Schur-product preservation of PSD; Horn-Johnson 2013 §7.5).

### §20.2 — Magnus K=4 with GL₂ sampling (CITATION + NORMATIVE)

The order-4 Magnus operator from §12.9 (Iserles+ 2000 §6 Method M₄, citing Blanes+ 2009 Table 5) is

```math
Ω_4(τ) = (τ/2) · (A₁ + A₂)  +  (√3 · τ² / 12) · [A₂, A₁],
```

with `A_i = −L_a(c_i · τ)` and GL₂ abscissae `c₁ = (3 − √3) / 6`, `c₂ = (3 + √3) / 6`. At each abscissa the library:

1. Calls `lap_at_t(c_i · τ)` → `Arc<Laplacian<F>>`.
2. Calls `a_at_t(c_i · τ)` → `Vec<F>` (length `N`).
3. Computes `sqrt_a_i[k] = a_i[k].sqrt()` (NORMATIVE: zero-allocation per step — pre-allocated buffer; `a < 0` returns `SemiflowError::DomainViolation`).
4. Builds `A_i v` via `apply_la_on_slice(L_G(c_i·τ), sqrt_a_i, v, out, tmp1, tmp2)`.

Then `exp(Ω_4(τ))` is applied via degree-4 Taylor truncation `Σ_{k=0}^{4} Ω_4^k / k!` (same kernel as `apply_exp_omega4_kernel` from `magnus_graph.rs:649`, factored to accept `&dyn Fn(&[F], &mut [F])` operator closure per ADR-0063).

### §20.3 — Convergence radius (NORMATIVE)

The matrix-Magnus convergence radius `∫₀^τ ‖A(s)‖₂ ds < π` (Blanes+ 2009 Theorem 1) lifts to `L_a(t)` via the operator-norm bound

```math
‖L_a(t)‖_2 ≤ ρ̄(L_G(t)) · a_{sup}(t)²,    a_{sup}(t) := max_i sqrt(a_i(t)) = sqrt(max_i a_i(t)).
```

The library imposes the **50% safety margin** (consistent with ADR-0051 / ADR-0056):

```math
ρ̄_max · a_{sup,max}² · τ < π / 2,
```

where `ρ̄_max := max_t ρ̄(L_G(t))` and `a_{sup,max} := max_t sqrt(max_i a_i(t))` over `t ∈ [0, τ]`, both supplied by the caller (or estimated via the optional `compute_rho_bar` helper — §20.5). Violations return `SemiflowError::OutOfMagnusRadius { tau, rho_estimate: ρ̄_max · a_{sup,max}² }`.

### §20.4 — Precision policy (NORMATIVE — ADR-0063)

Generic `<F: SemiflowFloat>`. The new operations beyond §12.9 K=4 are diagonal scaling (`sqrt` + element-wise multiplication), which preserves the order-of-magnitude coefficients of the Magnus expansion. Per ADR-0046 precision-policy bands, the f32 slope gate for `VarCoefMagnusGraphHeatChernoff` is ≤ −3.50, matching constant-coefficient K=4 (§12.9 G15 gate).

### §20.5 — `compute_rho_bar` helper (NORMATIVE — public API)

```rust
pub fn compute_rho_bar<F: SemiflowFloat>(
    lap_at_t: &LaplacianAtTime<F>,
    weight_at_t: &WeightAtTime<F>,
    interval: (F, F),
    n_samples: usize,  // recommended: 32
) -> (F, F);  // (rho_bar_max, a_sup_max)
```

Returns `(max_t ρ̄(L_G(t)), max_t sqrt(max_i a_i(t)))` over `n_samples` equispaced sample points in `interval`. **CITATION** for sampling-based supremum estimate: Higham 2008 §6 — power-iteration on `L_G(t)` gives a Gershgorin-bound-tight estimate of `ρ̄`. The library uses the cheaper `Laplacian::spectral_radius_bound()` per-sample.

### §20.6 — Acceptance gates (G22 + T17N)

- **G22 slope gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0063): time-dependent `P_64` with `L_G(t)` from `w(t) = 1 + 0.3·sin(πt)` and `a(t)` from `a_i(t) = 1 + 0.5·cos(πt) · i/N`, `t_final = 0.5`, `n_steps ∈ {5, 10, 20, 40, 80}`. Slope ≤ −3.85 (f64) / ≤ −3.50 (f32).
- **T17N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0063): on a symbolic 4×4 path Laplacian with symbolic `a(t)` polynomial and `w(t)` polynomial, verify `Ω_4(τ) − Ω_true(τ) = O(τ⁵)` (matching through τ⁴) via sympy series expansion. Pure symbolic; no library runtime.

### §20.7 — References

- §12 references (graph PDE + CSR storage).
- §14 references (variable-topology `L_G(t)`).
- §12.9 / ADR-0051 references (Magnus K=4 graph).
- R. A. Horn, C. R. Johnson, *Matrix Analysis* (2nd ed., Cambridge 2013), §7.5 — Schur product preserves PSD.

---

## §3.5.bis — `BoundaryPolicy` widening: stencil-BC vs operator-killing (v2.6, ADR-0068, NORMATIVE library)

§3.5 (v0.2.1) specified the four-variant `BoundaryPolicy` enum (`Reflect`, `ZeroExtend`, `Periodic`, `LinearExtrapolate`) governing how `Grid1D::sample(x)` extends an indexed grid function to a continuous function on `ℝ`. §3.5.bis (v2.6) widens the enum **additively** with two new variants — `Dirichlet { value: F }` and `Neumann` — and *normatively distinguishes* this stencil-level boundary policy from the operator-level Dirichlet via Feynman–Kac killing of §21.

Both ship in v2.6. They are mathematically distinct objects:

| Object | What it answers | Where it lives | When to use |
|---|---|---|---|
| Stencil-BC (§3.5 + §3.5.bis) — `BoundaryPolicy<F>` | "What value does `f̃(x)` take at `x ∉ [x_min, x_max]`?" | Adapter on `Grid1D`; consumed by `bc_value`. Pre-Chernoff. | The PDE's domain extends past the discretization grid; the operator's stencil needs values at ghost nodes. The BC is a *property of the interpolant*. |
| Operator-killing (§21) — `KillingChernoff<C, R>` | "What is the semigroup that absorbs trajectories on `∂R`?" | Wrapper around a `ChernoffFunction<F>` impl. Post-Chernoff. | The PDE is **defined** on a bounded region `R ⊊ ℝᴰ` with absorbing boundary on `∂R`; the operator itself is restricted (Feynman–Kac killing). The BC is a *property of the operator*. |

The discriminator: if the user has a PDE on `R = [a, b]` with `u(t, a) = u(t, b) = 0` (vanishing PDF, absorbing wall, killed Brownian motion), the **correct** v2.6 vehicle is `KillingChernoff<C, BoxRegion>` (§21). If the user has a PDE on all of `ℝ` discretized only on `[a, b]` for computational reasons and wants the ghost-node values clamped to a constant, the correct vehicle is `BoundaryPolicy::Dirichlet { value }`. Mixing the two (e.g., `KillingChernoff` with `BoundaryPolicy::ZeroExtend`) is mathematically valid but rarely needed — the killing wrapper dominates the convergence rate (order-1, §21.3).

### §3.5.bis.1 — `Dirichlet { value: F }` (v2.6, NEW)

**Continuous form.** Constant extension at both endpoints to the user-supplied scalar `c := value`:
$$
\widetilde{f}(x) =
\begin{cases}
c, & x < x_{\min}, \\
f(x), & x_{\min} \le x \le x_{\max}, \\
c, & x > x_{\max}.
\end{cases}
$$
$\widetilde{f}$ is $C^0$ on $\mathbb{R}$ iff $f(x_{\min}) = f(x_{\max}) = c$ (the *consistent-data* case); otherwise discontinuous with jump magnitudes $|f(x_{\min}) - c|$ at the left and $|f(x_{\max}) - c|$ at the right. **Use case**: clamped-to-zero ghost-node extension when the initial datum is non-zero at the boundary but the user knows the true solution is held at `c` on the boundary for all $t$ (e.g., heat equation with non-zero Dirichlet boundary data via the inhomogeneous-to-homogeneous reduction).

**Discrete index form.** Add a new `BoundaryHit::Dirichlet(F)` payload variant in `traits.yaml` §4. `bc_index` for `Dirichlet { value }` returns `Inside(j as usize)` for $j \in [0, n)$, else `BoundaryHit::Dirichlet(value)`. Downstream `bc_value` returns `value` on `Dirichlet(value)`. **Generic over `F`** via the enum type parameter `BoundaryPolicy<F = f64>` (ADR-0025 default; legacy call sites compile unchanged).

**Cubic-Hermite stability.** When the stencil straddles the boundary the four control points include hard `c`-values, producing an over- or under-shoot whose magnitude depends on the jump $|f(x_{\min}) - c|$. For the consistent-data case ($c = f(x_{\min})$) the behaviour reduces to `ZeroExtend` shifted by $c$ — overshoot envelope $\tfrac{1}{8}|f(x_{\min}) - c|$ per Catmull-Rom Lebesgue constant. For inconsistent-data the boundary becomes a fixed-step discontinuity; **NOT acceptable** for high-frequency boundary-active data.

### §3.5.bis.2 — `Neumann` (v2.6, NEW)

**Continuous form.** Constant extension at both endpoints to the boundary value (i.e., zero-flux / zero-derivative boundary condition realized as a flat ghost extension):
$$
\widetilde{f}(x) =
\begin{cases}
f(x_{\min}), & x < x_{\min}, \\
f(x), & x_{\min} \le x \le x_{\max}, \\
f(x_{\max}), & x > x_{\max}.
\end{cases}
$$
$\widetilde{f}$ is unconditionally $C^0$ on $\mathbb{R}$ (no jump). $\widetilde{f}$ is $C^1$ at the boundary iff $f'(x_{\min}^+) = 0$ and $f'(x_{\max}^-) = 0$ (the *consistent-Neumann-data* case). **Use case**: zero-flux insulated boundary, reflecting random walk, image-method reflected heat (v2.8 B4 prep).

**Discrete index form.** `bc_index` for `Neumann` returns `Inside(j as usize)` for $j \in [0, n)$, `Inside(0)` for $j < 0$, and `Inside(n-1)` for $j \ge n$ (constant-extension via clamp to the boundary node). Returns the existing `BoundaryHit::Inside(i)` shape — no new payload variant needed for Neumann. **Non-parameterized** unit variant; does not affect the enum's generic-over-`F` shape (lifts to `BoundaryPolicy<F>` cleanly).

**Cubic-Hermite stability.** Clamp-to-boundary stencil collapses the four control points $\{i-1, i, i+1, i+2\}$ near the right boundary at $i = n-1$ to $\{n-1, n-1, n-1, n-1\}$ — Catmull-Rom on degenerate control polygon evaluates to a constant. The discrete derivative at the boundary is **exactly zero** (slope formula divides by $0$ would arise; the constant-extension dispatch never invokes the slope formula). **No oscillation**. This matches the physical Neumann BC and is the discrete analogue of the v0.1.0 `Reflect` policy in the symmetric-data case but *unconditionally* for any input data.

### §3.5.bis.3 — Cross-references and policy-selection guide

| Use case | Recommended policy |
|---|---|
| Heat equation on `[-10, 10]` with compactly-supported Gaussian initial datum (G1/G2/G3 oracles) | `Reflect` (existing — preserves Gaussian decay) |
| Heat equation on `[0, 1]` with absorbing boundary `u(0) = u(1) = 0` (eigenmode oracle, B3) | `KillingChernoff<C, BoxRegion>` (§21) — *not* `Dirichlet { value: 0.0 }` |
| Heat equation on `[a, b]` with insulated boundary `∂u/∂n = 0` (reflected diffusion) | `Neumann` (this section) — equivalent to `Reflect` for the diffusion stencil but cleaner intent expression |
| Sine wave on `[-π, π]` periodically extended | `Periodic` (existing) |
| Affine boundary data `u(x) ≈ αx + β` at the boundary | `LinearExtrapolate` (existing) |
| Non-zero constant Dirichlet `u(0) = u(1) = c` (inhomogeneous reduction) | `Dirichlet { value: c }` (this section) |

All six policies satisfy the I5 strict-interior agreement invariant (§3.5; for $i \in [0, n)$ and any policy, `bc_index(policy, n, i) == Inside(i)`). All six are TOTAL over `(BoundaryPolicy<F>, n ≥ 2, idx ∈ i64)` (I1 extended). The two new variants are gated by the new property `bc_index_dirichlet_neumann_totality` (cases: 1000) in `properties.yaml`.

### §3.5.bis.4 — Module relocation note (NORMATIVE — ADR-0068)

The implementation of `BoundaryPolicy`, `BoundaryHit`, `bc_index`, `bc_value`, `bc_value_generic`, and `reflect_index` MOVES from `crates/semiflow-core/src/grid.rs` to a NEW module `crates/semiflow-core/src/boundary.rs` at v2.6. Public re-exports preserve the v2.5.1 import path (`use semiflow_core::BoundaryPolicy`); no user code is affected. Rationale: `grid.rs` is at 715/715 LoC against its Override #1 carve-out; the v2.6 widening would force another cap expansion. Extracting `boundary.rs` (estimated ≤500 LoC, within default suckless cap) shrinks `grid.rs` back below the original 700 cap and obviates further carve-out expansion. See ADR-0068 §"Consequences" and constitution amendment v1.6.1 → v1.6.2.

---

## §3.5.tris — Robin BC partial-additive port (v4.6, ADR-0098, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §3.5.tris.1 — Scope and verdict

For a self-adjoint second-order operator $L$ (e.g., $L = \partial_{xx}$ for 1D heat) on a domain $R \subset \mathbb{R}^d$ with boundary $\partial R$, the **Robin boundary problem** is
$$
\partial_t u(t, x) = L u(t, x) \text{ in } (0, \infty) \times R, \qquad \alpha\, u(t, x) + \beta\, \partial_\nu u(t, x)|_{x \in \partial R} = 0, \qquad u(0, x) = f(x), \tag{3.5.tris.1}
$$
with $\alpha \ge 0$, $\beta > 0$, $\alpha + \beta > 0$ (well-posedness; see Engel-Nagel 2000 Ch. VI §6). The two singular limits recover the established cases:
- $\alpha = 0$ (pure Neumann): see §25 (`ReflectedHeatChernoff`, image method, order-preserving).
- $\beta = 0$ (pure Dirichlet): see §21 (`KillingChernoff`, Feynman-Kac killing, order-1 cap).

v2.6 ADR-0068 widened `BoundaryPolicy` with `Dirichlet`+`Neumann`; v2.8 ADR-0072 shipped operator-level Neumann via image method (§25). Robin was explicitly DEFERRED in §25.7 ("Engel 2003 active research; the image method does NOT extend uniformly to Robin"). v4.6 ADR-0098 ships the **partial-additive** static Robin via skew-reflection (research1.md Part B Vector 4 verdict — Carslaw-Jaeger 1959 §3.4 + §14.2) (reimplemented stencil-level in v6.2.3, ADR-0098 Amendment 2). The **dynamic** Robin BC ($\partial_t u + \partial_\nu u = 0$ on $\partial \Omega$ requiring boundary-clock state-space lift $X \oplus L^2(\partial \Omega)$ per Engel 2003 *Studia Math.*) remains UNSHIPPED and DEFERRED INDEFINITELY (§3.5.tris.6).

### §3.5.tris.2 — Exact 1D half-line Robin kernel (CITATION — Carslaw-Jaeger 1959 §14.2 eq 5)

For the half-line $R = [0, \infty)$ with Robin BC $\alpha u(0) + \beta u'(0) = 0$, the *exact* Robin heat kernel is
$$
K^{\mathrm{Robin}}(x, y; t) \;=\; K(x, y; t) \;+\; K(x, -y; t) \;-\; \frac{\alpha}{\beta}\, e^{(\alpha/\beta)(x+y) + (\alpha/\beta)^2 t}\,\mathrm{erfc}\!\left(\frac{x+y}{2\sqrt{t}} + \frac{\alpha}{\beta}\sqrt{t}\right), \tag{3.5.tris.2}
$$
where $K(x, y; t) := (4 \pi t)^{-1/2} \exp\!\big({-(x-y)^2 / (4t)}\big)$ is the free-space heat kernel. The third term (erfc-correction) is the genuine multiplier that distinguishes Robin from a naive scalar-multiplied ghost; setting $\alpha = 0$ collapses it to zero (pure Neumann recovery). This formula is the **G_ROBIN_HALFLINE oracle** (evaluated via `libm::erfc` to machine precision).

### §3.5.tris.3 — Stencil-level skew image extension (NORMATIVE library, v6.2.3 ADR-0098 Amendment 2)

The Robin half-line semigroup is realized by the free-space semigroup acting on the **skew (exponentially-weighted) even extension** $E_R$:

$$
(E_R u)(x) \;:=\; \begin{cases} u(x) & x \ge 0, \\ e^{-2(\alpha/\beta)(-x)}\,u(-x) & x < 0. \end{cases} \tag{3.5.tris.3}
$$

Then $S^{\mathrm{Robin}}(t) u = \bigl(e^{t\Delta}_{\mathrm{free}}\,E_R u\bigr)\big|_{[0,\infty)}$. Differentiating at $0^-$ gives $\partial_x(E_R u)(0^-) = u'(0) - 2(\alpha/\beta)u(0)$, enforcing $\alpha u(0) - \beta u'(0) = 0$ (the Robin condition; outward normal $\partial_\nu = -\partial_x$ at $x = 0$).

**Limits**: $\alpha = 0 \Rightarrow$ weight $1$ = even reflection (pure Neumann, §25). $\alpha/\beta \to \infty \Rightarrow$ weight $0$ = absorbing (Dirichlet, §21).

**Discretization**: a stencil sampling signed index $\mathrm{idx} = -d$ ($d \ge 1$, position $-d\,dx$) reads the ghost value

$$
u_{-d} \;=\; w^{(d)}\,u_d, \qquad w^{(d)} = e^{-2(\alpha/\beta)\,d\,dx} = q^d, \quad q = e^{-2(\alpha/\beta)\,dx}. \tag{3.5.tris.4}
$$

The single-cell central-difference form $u_{-1} = u_1 - 2\,dx\,(\alpha/\beta)\,u_0$ is only the $d=1$ Taylor truncation and is INSUFFICIENT for the Chernoff Gaussian-average kernel (offsets $\pm 2\sqrt{a\tau}$ reach depths $d = O(\sqrt{\tau}/dx) \gg 1$); the exponential form is exact at all depths. The continuous convolution of $E_R u$ with the free Gaussian yields exactly the §3.5.tris.2 Carslaw-Jaeger kernel (factor $\alpha/\beta$), so the discrete scheme converges to the oracle at order 1.

### §3.5.tris.4 — Per-step algorithm (NORMATIVE library, v6.2.3 ADR-0098 Amendment 2)

```
RobinHeatChernoff::apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch):
  1. (α, β) := region.robin_coeffs()
  2. src_robin := src with grid.boundary = BoundaryPolicy::Robin{α, β}
  3. inner.apply_into(τ, src_robin, dst, scratch)   // single step; BC handled in stencil sampler
```

The Robin character is supplied by `bc_index` → `BoundaryHit::RobinSkew{reflected, depth}` for out-of-range indices, and by `bc_value`/`bc_value_generic` applying $w^{(d)} = e^{-2(\alpha/\beta)\,d\,dx}$ (mirrors §25 Neumann, which uses weight $\equiv 1$). Per-call cost **halved** vs the old 4-step ($1 \times$ inner cost; no ghost/tmp buffers).

### §3.5.tris.5 — Order analysis and acceptance gates (G_ROBIN_HALFLINE + G_ROBIN_SELF + T_ROBIN — NORMATIVE)

**Order result**: `RobinHeatChernoff::order() = 1`. The skew extension $\mathbf{1}_R + r \cdot \mathbf{1}_R \circ \sigma_R$ has a NONZERO commutator with self-adjoint $L$ for any $r \ne 1$. Proposition 25.1 (Neumann order-preservation) does NOT extend to Robin; the wrapper is order-1 by construction (consistent with the Chernoff product floor for non-symmetric BCs). Higher-order Robin (e.g., order-2 via Strang-style symmetrisation) is v5.x+ research (§3.5.tris.6).

- **G_ROBIN_HALFLINE** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0098): 1D half-line $R = [0, 10]$ (truncation of $[0, \infty)$) with $(\alpha, \beta) = (1.0, 1.0)$ mixed reference and Gaussian initial datum $g(x) = \exp(-x^2)$ on $R$. Oracle: $u_{\mathrm{Robin}}(T, x) = \int_0^\infty K^{\mathrm{Robin}}(x, y; T) g(y)\, dy$ at $T = 0.1$, with $K^{\mathrm{Robin}}$ per (3.5.tris.2) evaluated via `libm::erfc`. Spatial grid n_grid = 512 (raised from 64 in v6.2.3 so the $O(dx)$ skew-BC spatial floor stays subdominant to the temporal Chernoff error). Sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ (Chernoff steps); empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|F^n(g) - u_{\mathrm{Robin}}(T, \cdot)\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST satisfy $\le -0.95$ (order-1 gate; measured slope $-1.13$). Threshold $-0.95$ unchanged. Test file: `tests/robin_heat_slope.rs` (feature `slow-tests`).
- **G_ROBIN_SELF** (DEFERRED to v6.3.0 — ADR-0098 Amendment 2): 2D self-convergence on box $[0, 1]^2$ with Robin BC on all four walls; Strang per-axis composition; no closed-form oracle (mirror v2.2 G_NS2D_aniso pattern). Deferred pending full Strang per-axis Robin composition implementation. Gate is a non-panicking `#[ignore]` stub in `tests/robin_heat_slope.rs` (the prior `todo!()` latent-panic removed in v6.2.3).
- **T_ROBIN** (NORMATIVE sympy — ADR-0098): 4 mandatory sub-checks: (a) Neumann-limit verification: exact kernel $K^{\mathrm{Robin}}$ with $\alpha=0$ equals the Neumann kernel (erfc correction vanishes); (b) Robin BC $\alpha K + \beta \partial_x K = 0$ at $x = 0$ satisfied EXACTLY (symbolic `subs(x, 0) + simplify` → literally zero); (c) heat-PDE residual $\partial_t K = \partial_{xx} K$; (d) numerical cross-check `sympy(K_Robin)` vs `libm::erfc(K_Robin)` at sample point $(x, y, t, \alpha, \beta) = (1.0, 0.5, 0.1, 1.0, 1.0)$ within $10^{-12}$ relative tolerance. Script: `scripts/verify_robin_kernel.py` (integrated into `test-fast` sympy sweep). MUST print exactly `T_ROBIN PASS`. Failure BLOCKS release.

### §3.5.tris.6 — Limitations and future work

- **Robin order capped at 1** (skew commutator non-vanishing). Strang-style symmetric splitting `r^{1/2}-step → inner → r^{1/2}-step` may reach order 2 but requires per-step square-root of the skew coefficient; deferred to v5.x research (`[[project-robin-higher-order]]`).
- **Dynamic Robin BC UNSHIPPED** ($\partial_t u + \partial_\nu u = 0$ on $\partial \Omega$): requires boundary-clock state-space lift $X \oplus L^2(\partial \Omega)$ per Engel 2003 *Studia Math.* The Chernoff construction in this setting is non-standardised (Goldstein-Engel active research per research1.md Part B Vector 4 §c). DEFERRED INDEFINITELY.
- **Multi-D Robin with per-cell varying $(\alpha, \beta)$**: v4.6 ships scalar $(\alpha, \beta)$ constant across $\partial R$. Per-cell spatial variation $(\alpha(x), \beta(x))$ requires `RobinRegion::robin_coeffs_at(point)` extension; v5.x scope.
- **Reflection requires self-adjoint $L$.** Same caveat as Neumann (§25.7); non-self-adjoint $L$ may degrade order further. Documented in rustdoc.

### §3.5.tris.7 — References

- H. S. Carslaw & J. C. Jaeger, *Conduction of Heat in Solids* (2nd ed.), Oxford University Press, 1959. §3.4 (image method short-time skew-r derivation); §14.2 eq 5 (exact 3-term Robin heat kernel with erfc-correction — the G_ROBIN_HALFLINE oracle).
- J. B. Walsh, *Markov Processes and Potential Theory*, in *École d'Été de Probabilités de Saint-Flour XIV — 1984*, Springer LNM **1180** (1986), pp. 265–439. §3.4 — image-method generalisation to skew reflection (Robin extension of (25.2)).
- K.-J. Engel & R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations*, Springer GTM **194** (2000). Ch. VI §6 — Robin generator characterisation; analytic-semigroup theory.
- K.-J. Engel, *Dynamic boundary conditions for second order differential operators*, **Studia Math.** 158:2 (2003), 113–127. — Boundary-clock state-space lift for dynamic Robin BC (out-of-scope; DEFERRED INDEFINITELY).
- Y. A. Butko, H. Grothaus, O. G. Smolyanov, *Lagrangian Feynman formulas for second-order parabolic equations in bounded domains*, **Infin. Dimens. Anal. Quantum Probab. Relat. Top.** 13:3 (2010), 377–392. — Reflected-diffusion image-method foundations.

---

## §3.6.bis — L-gate (latency gate) acceptance-gate semantics (v2.6, ADR-0068, NORMATIVE library)

### §3.6.bis.1 — Definition

An **L-gate** (latency gate) is a `properties.yaml` acceptance gate whose assertion takes the form
$$
\text{Pct}_p\!\big[\,T_{\text{op}}(\text{input}; \text{profile})\,\big] \;\le\; B_p,
\qquad p \in \{50, 99, 99.9, 99.99\}
$$
where:

- $T_{\text{op}}(\text{input}; \text{profile})$ is the *wall-clock per-operation latency* of a designated benchmark binary (an `examples/*.rs` or `benches/*.rs` target), measured in nanoseconds with monotonic-clock granularity, over $N$ repeated invocations on a fixed input (canonical seed, fixed parameters);
- $\text{Pct}_p[\cdot]$ is the **NIST nearest-rank percentile** (ASTM E29-13 §6, formula $r = \lceil (p/100) \cdot N \rceil$) of the latency sample;
- $\text{profile}$ is a **hardware profile identifier** (a string key in the L-gate schema, e.g., `"i7-12700K"`) that resolves to a CPU + clock-domain + thermal envelope + governor specification (`/sys/devices/system/cpu/intel_pstate/no_turbo == 0`, `cpufreq/scaling_governor == performance`, ambient temperature ≤ 25 °C, ≥ 5 minutes warm-up);
- $B_p$ is the per-percentile budget in nanoseconds, calibrated from a baseline measurement on the named profile plus a documented headroom (typically 10%–20%).

An L-gate **passes** for a (profile, percentile) pair if and only if all percentiles in the entry's `percentile_budgets_ns` map satisfy the inequality. An L-gate **fails-advisory** in v2.6 (the harness emits warnings; exit code 0) and **fails-blocking** in v2.7+ (the harness returns non-zero exit; CI fails). Per-profile entries marked `status: advisory` in `properties.yaml` are advisory regardless of release version (used for placeholder profiles before calibration data exists).

### §3.6.bis.2 — Why L-gates are distinct from `properties:` gates

The existing `properties:` schema (G1..G22, T1N..T17N, all `STRANG*_BIT_EQUAL`, `SIMD_*`) asserts mathematical / contractual invariants: sup-norm tolerance, log-log slope, bit-equality, contractivity. L-gates assert **operational percentile bounds**, with three distinguishing properties:

1. **Host-dependence is intrinsic.** A property like "Strang2D slope ≤ −1.95" is host-independent (passes on any reasonable f64 machine). A latency gate "p99.9 ≤ 50ns" is meaningful only with the hardware profile fully specified — a clock-down to 800 MHz or a context switch into a co-tenant noisy neighbour invalidates the assertion class, not the measurement.
2. **Replication is intrinsic.** A property gate is a binary pass/fail on a single canonical run. An L-gate is a percentile over $N$ replications (canonically $N \ge 1{,}000$, ideally $\ge 1{,}000{,}000$ for tail percentiles like p99.99).
3. **Calibration is a contract artefact.** The budget $B_p$ for each (gate, profile, percentile) is derived from a *baseline measurement* recorded in the L-gate entry (`baseline_p999_ns: 45` for `L_CEV_PTICK`, calibrated from the ADR-0067 measurement on `i7-12700K`) plus a documented headroom factor. Re-calibration after a hardware change is a `properties.yaml` schema bump, recorded in the version-history table (ADR-0068 §"Consequences").

### §3.6.bis.3 — Schema (NORMATIVE)

L-gate entries live under a new top-level `latency_gates:` section in `properties.yaml`. Schema, mirroring the style of the existing `properties:` list:

```yaml
latency_gates:
  - id: <STRING>                  # e.g., "L_CEV_PTICK"
    severity: <ENUM>              # ADVISORY | NORMATIVE | RELEASE_BLOCKING
    bench_target: <STRING>        # e.g., "examples/latency_tail.rs"
    bench_invocation: <STRING>    # full cargo invocation string
    measurement: <STRING>         # what is being measured (e.g., "per-tick CEV pricing latency")
    canonical_input:              # the fixed input the bench loads
      seed: <STRING>              # PCG64 / xoshiro seed identifier
      n: <INT>                    # input length
      sha256: <STRING>            # canonical-input sha256 (reproducibility)
    replication:
      n_reps: <INT>               # bench replications (>= 5)
      n_per_rep: <INT>            # observations per rep (>= 1000)
      warmup: <INT>               # warmup ops discarded before measurement
    percentile_budgets_ns:
      "i7-12700K":                # per-profile budget map
        p50: <INT>
        p99: <INT>
        p999: <INT>
        p9999: <INT>
        baseline_p999_ns: <INT>   # the calibrated baseline
        headroom_pct: <INT>       # headroom factor used to derive budget
        status: blocking          # or "advisory" for placeholder profiles
        calibrated_at: <ISO8601>
        calibrated_from_adr: <STRING>  # e.g., "ADR-0067"
      "m2-pro":                   # placeholder profile (advisory until calibrated)
        status: advisory
        p999: null
    output_format: jsonl          # bench emits JSONL per rep
    parser: hdr_snapshot          # hdr_snapshot OR custom field name
    purpose: |
      Free-text rationale + cross-refs to ADRs / oracle papers.
    feature_gate: <STRING>        # e.g., "release" (release build required)
```

Each `percentile_budgets_ns` entry MAY have `status: advisory` (placeholder; treated as informational regardless of severity) or `status: blocking` (assertion live in v2.6 with severity-dependent enforcement: ADVISORY = warning, NORMATIVE / RELEASE_BLOCKING = error). For v2.6 the harness treats every L-gate as advisory regardless of severity (CI does not fail on L-gate breach). The v2.7 promotion bumps `L_CEV_PTICK.severity` to `RELEASE_BLOCKING` and removes the v2.6-only advisory clamp.

### §3.6.bis.4 — Harness contract (`xtask latency-gate`)

The `xtask latency-gate <gate_id> [--hardware-profile <profile>]` subcommand:

1. Reads `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` and locates the `latency_gates:` entry by `id`.
2. Resolves `--hardware-profile` against the entry's `percentile_budgets_ns` map; if the profile is absent or `status: advisory`, the harness emits an informational message and exits 0.
3. Runs `bench_invocation` (subprocess), capturing the bench's stdout JSONL stream and the canonical-input sha256 verification.
4. Parses the JSONL into an `HdrSnapshot<i64>` (per `traits.yaml` §4 below) — one snapshot per rep.
5. Pools the across-rep percentiles via the median-of-percentiles (robust to one slow rep, consistent with the v2.5.1 `latency_tail.rs` aggregation).
6. For each percentile $p$ in the profile's budget map, asserts $\text{Pct}_p \le B_p$. On breach: severity ADVISORY → stderr warning, exit 0; severity NORMATIVE → stderr warning, exit 0 (v2.6 transitional); severity RELEASE_BLOCKING → stderr error, exit 1 (v2.7+).
7. Writes the measurement to `.dev-docs/reports/latency-gates/<gate_id>-<profile>-<timestamp>.json` for the v2.7 multi-host calibration table.

### §3.6.bis.5 — Provenance and lineage

The L-gate concept is the contract-side complement of ADR-0066 (`tracking-alloc` feature — measures *space*) and ADR-0067 (`latency_tail.rs` example — measures *time*). The v2.5.1 release reported the `L_CEV_PTICK` baseline (p99.9 = 45 ns, p99 = 32 ns, p50 = 23 ns; 149× advantage vs QuantLib V3 Schroder ncx2 at matched accuracy) but had no machine-readable contract that asserts these numbers. §3.6.bis closes that gap; L-gates make the latency baseline a first-class element of the acceptance suite, on par with the convergence-slope gates.

### §3.6.bis.6 — References

- ASTM E29-13 §6 — nearest-rank percentile definition (NIST-compatible).
- ADR-0066 — `tracking-alloc` feature (per-tick allocation measurement).
- ADR-0067 — `latency_tail.rs` example (v2.5.1 baseline measurement).
- ADR-0068 — this section's authorizing ADR.

### §3.6.bis.7 — v2.7 Amendment (ADR-0069): per-gate `advisory:` field becomes load-bearing

The v2.6 base text above (§3.6.bis.1 — §3.6.bis.6) defines the L-gate schema and the harness contract. The per-profile field `percentile_budgets_ns.<profile>.advisory: <bool>` was *declared* in v2.6 but *not enforced*: the v2.6 harness (xtask/src/latency_gate.rs) clamped every L-gate to advisory-mode (warn + exit 0) regardless of `advisory:` or `severity:`. This was the v2.6 transitional behaviour, documented in §3.6.bis.4 step 6.

**v2.7 promotes the `advisory:` field to load-bearing** (ADR-0069). The harness now reads the per-profile `advisory:` flag and dispatches enforcement as follows:

| `severity:` (entry-level) | per-profile `advisory:` | Floor breach action |
|---|---|---|
| `ADVISORY` | any | stderr warning; exit 0 |
| `NORMATIVE` | `true` (or unset; default true) | stderr warning; exit 0 |
| `NORMATIVE` | `false` | stderr warning; exit 0 *(NORMATIVE is documentary, not CI-blocking)* |
| `RELEASE_BLOCKING` | `true` (or unset; default true) | stderr warning; exit 0 |
| `RELEASE_BLOCKING` | `false` | stderr error; **exit 1** |

The default-if-absent rule is `advisory: true` (backward-compatible: any v2.6 entry that does not declare the field continues to behave as advisory and does not break CI on v2.7). Explicit `advisory: false` is required to opt a profile into blocking enforcement.

**v2.7 promotes one gate to blocking**: `L_CEV_PTICK` `percentile_budgets_ns.i7-12700K.advisory: true → false` (explicit edit in `properties.yaml`, recorded in CHANGELOG). The other profiles (`m2-pro`, `aws-c7g-large`) remain `advisory: true` placeholders until calibration samples are collected. The v2.7 release also adds:

- `L_RESOLVENT_N64_P99` — new gate per ADR-0069 for the Laplace-Chernoff resolvent (`crates/semiflow-core/examples/resolvent_perf.rs`). `i7-12700K.advisory: true` in v2.7.0-rc.1 (one RC cycle of calibration); `advisory: false` in v2.7.0 final.
- `L_HESTON_PTICK` — new gate for the HFT Heston pricer side-track example (`crates/semiflow-core/examples/heston_pricer.rs`). `i7-12700K.advisory: true` throughout v2.7 (calibration deferred to v2.8 if Heston usage stabilises). No promotion in v2.7.

Schema-version impact: `properties.yaml` 0.8.0 → 0.9.0. The bump is justified by the load-bearing semantics change to an existing field, not by new schema keys (the field already existed in v2.6 but had no enforcement effect).

Cross-references: ADR-0069 §"Consequences" (the L-gate promotion mechanics in xtask/src/latency_gate.rs); ADR-0070 (companion v2.7 ADR; no new L-gate); CHANGELOG v2.7.0 entry.

---

## §21 — Operator-level Dirichlet via Feynman–Kac killing (v2.6, ADR-0068, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §21.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

Many problems in mathematical physics and finance require a semigroup that is *defined on a bounded region* `R ⊊ ℝᴰ` with **absorbing boundary** on `∂R` — e.g., killed Brownian motion on the unit interval, vanishing PDF of a first-exit time, barrier-option pricing. These problems are not solved by stencil-level boundary policies (§3.5, §3.5.bis): a `BoundaryPolicy::Dirichlet { value: 0.0 }` zeros out ghost-node values for the *spatial interpolant*, but the operator's discrete propagator (e.g., `DiffusionChernoff::apply`) still treats interior nodes as if the domain were `ℝ`. Trajectories that should have been killed at `∂R` continue to contribute to interior values, biasing the solution by an O(1) systematic error.

The mathematical fix is the **Feynman–Kac killing functional**:
$$
(P^R_t f)(x) := \mathbb{E}^x\!\left[\,f(X_t) \cdot \mathbb{1}_{\{\tau_R > t\}}\,\right],
\qquad \tau_R := \inf\{s \ge 0 : X_s \notin R\},
$$
where $X_t$ is the diffusion generated by the unrestricted operator $L$ and $\tau_R$ is the first exit time. The semigroup $\{P^R_t\}_{t \ge 0}$ is the strongly-continuous semigroup with generator $L|_{D(L^R)}$ where $D(L^R) := \{f \in D(L) : f|_{\partial R} = 0\}$ (the Dirichlet realization of $L$ on $R$).

### §21.2 — Chernoff approximation of the killed semigroup (CITATION — Butko 2018)

Butko (2018, *Fract. Calc. Appl. Anal.* 21:5) proves that for any Chernoff function $C(\tau)$ approximating $e^{\tau L}$ on a core $D \subset D(L)$ with consistency order $m \ge 1$, the **killed Chernoff function**
$$
F(\tau) f \;:=\; \mathbb{1}_R \cdot C(\tau) f \;\;\;\text{(post-multiply, pointwise)}
$$
is a Chernoff function for $P^R_t$, with *globally degraded consistency order $m_{\text{killed}} = 1$* regardless of the inner $m$. The degradation is intrinsic to the killing functional: $\mathbb{1}_R$ is discontinuous on $\partial R$ and the commutator $[L, \mathbb{1}_R]$ contributes an irreducible $\mathcal{O}(\tau)$ term to the truncation error. Butko §3.2 derives the explicit constant.

**Specifically** (Butko 2018, eq. 3.7): for $f \in D(L) \cap L^\infty(R)$ with $\text{supp}(f) \subset \overline{R}$ and $\partial R$ Lipschitz,
$$
\|(F(\tau))^n f - P^R_{n\tau} f\|_{L^\infty(R)} \;\le\; K \cdot \tau \cdot \|f\|_{C^1(R)} \cdot (1 + \rho(L) \cdot n\tau)
$$
for a constant $K$ depending only on $R$ (specifically on the Lipschitz norm of $\partial R$). The slope-test discretization of this bound gives spatial convergence rate $\mathcal{O}(\Delta x)$ globally — see G23 acceptance gate (§21.5).

**Pre-multiply alternative is rejected** (NORMATIVE library choice): the alternative form $F'(\tau) f := C(\tau)(\mathbb{1}_R \cdot f)$ zeros out the input at boundary cells *before* the Chernoff stencil acts, so the stencil's interior cells lose contributions from boundary cells (over-killing). Butko §2.3 derives the asymmetry; post-multiply is the correct form. The library MUST NOT implement the pre-multiply variant.

### §21.3 — `KillingChernoff<C, R>` wrapper (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct KillingChernoff<C, R> {
    inner: C,
    region: R,
}

impl<C, R, F> ChernoffFunction<F> for KillingChernoff<C, R>
where
    F: SemiflowFloat,
    C: ChernoffFunction<F>,
    R: KillingRegion<F>,
{
    type S = C::S;

    fn apply_into(&self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        self.inner.apply_into(tau, src, dst)?;
        self.region.mask_in_place(dst)?;  // post-multiply by 1_R
        Ok(())
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 { 1 }  // killing dominates — Butko 2018 §3.2

    fn growth(&self) -> (f64, f64) {
        // 1_R is a contraction (||1_R · f||_∞ ≤ ||f||_∞); inherit inner growth.
        self.inner.growth()
    }
}
```

The `apply` convenience method (default impl on the `ChernoffFunction` trait) is inherited unchanged. The wrapper is **transparent to the inner** Chernoff function: composing `KillingChernoff<Strang2D<DiffusionChernoff, DiffusionChernoff>, BoxRegion<f64, 2>>` is a valid construction.

The `KillingRegion<F>` trait:

```rust
pub trait KillingRegion<F: SemiflowFloat> {
    /// Test whether a point is inside the killing region R.
    fn is_inside(&self, point: &[F]) -> bool;

    /// Apply the indicator mask to a state in-place: dst[i] = 0 for points outside R.
    /// Default impl iterates is_inside per cell; concrete impls MAY override for SIMD batch paths.
    fn mask_in_place<S: State<F>>(&self, dst: &mut S) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;

    /// Spatial dimension D of the region (informational; used by oracle calibration).
    fn dim(&self) -> usize;
}
```

Default `mask_in_place` calls `is_inside` per cell. The `BoxRegion` and `BallRegion` reference impls override `mask_in_place` with vectorized per-axis bound checks (no SIMD intrinsics in v2.6; scalar tight loops sufficient for the eigenmode oracle).

### §21.4 — Shipped regions (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct BoxRegion<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize> {
    pub lo: [F; D],
    pub hi: [F; D],
}
// is_inside: forall k in 0..D, lo[k] <= point[k] <= hi[k]

pub struct BallRegion<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize> {
    pub center: [F; D],
    pub radius: F,
}
// is_inside: sum_{k=0..D} (point[k] - center[k])^2 <= radius^2
```

Both impl `KillingRegion<F>`. Both use compile-time-known dimension `D` for zero-overhead dispatch. The shipped impls assume `R` is **open** (boundary cells where the indicator transitions are *excluded*); the engineering wave's `mask_in_place` MUST follow this convention exactly (returning `0.0` for cells *on* `∂R`). Half-spaces (degenerate `BoxRegion` with `hi[k] = +∞`), polyhedra, and user-defined `KillingRegion` impls are out of scope for v2.6 and tracked for v2.8 alongside the manifold pillar.

### §21.5 — Acceptance gates (G23 + T18N — NORMATIVE)

- **G23 slope gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0068): Heat equation $\partial_t u = \tfrac{1}{2} \partial_{xx} u$ on $R = (0, 1) \subset \mathbb{R}$ with absorbing boundary $u(t, 0) = u(t, 1) = 0$ and smooth initial datum $u(0, x) = \sum_{k=1}^{8} a_k \sin(k\pi x)$ with random coefficients $a_k \in [-1, 1]$. The closed-form eigenmode oracle is
  $$
  u(t, x) \;=\; \sum_{k=1}^{8} a_k \sin(k\pi x) \exp(-(k\pi)^2 \cdot t / 2).
  $$
  `KillingChernoff<DiffusionChernoff(a=0.5), BoxRegion<f64, 1> { lo: [0.0], hi: [1.0] }>` is slope-tested against this oracle. Sweep: $N \in \{64, 128, 256, 512\}$ at $T = 0.05$, $n_{\text{steps}} = 100$. **Slope ≤ −0.95** (order-1 globally per Butko 2018 §3.2). Test file: `tests/killing_dirichlet_slope.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v2.6 release.

- **T18N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0068): on the eigenmode expansion above, verify symbolically with sympy:
  1. Each individual mode $\sin(k\pi x)$ satisfies the boundary condition: $\sin(k\pi \cdot 0) = 0$ AND $\sin(k\pi \cdot 1) = 0$ for $k = 1, 2, 3, 4$.
  2. Each individual mode is an eigenfunction of $\tfrac{1}{2} \partial_{xx}$ with eigenvalue $-(k\pi)^2 / 2$ (sympy `diff(sin(k*pi*x), x, 2) / 2 == -(k*pi)**2 / 2 * sin(k*pi*x)` for $k = 1..4$).
  3. The eigenmode-superposition oracle satisfies $\partial_t u = \tfrac{1}{2} \partial_{xx} u$ symbolically.
  4. The Butko §3.2 commutator $[\tfrac{1}{2} \partial_{xx}, \mathbb{1}_R]$ vanishes on the *open* interior $R = (0, 1)$ (consistency check that the order-1 degradation is a boundary-only phenomenon).

  Script: `scripts/verify_killing_dirichlet.py` (new file, ~150 LoC, ships in engineering wave). MUST print `T18N PASS` on success or `T18N FAIL: <reason>` on failure. Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep.

### §21.6 — Limitations and future work

- **Order-1 only.** Higher-order killing Chernoff functions (order-2 via Strang-style symmetrization $\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2} \cdot C(\tau) \cdot \mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}$) are an open research direction (Butko 2018 §5 conjecture). v2.6 ships order-1; v2.9+ may revisit.
- **Lipschitz `∂R` only.** Butko's bound requires the boundary's Lipschitz norm to be finite; fractal or cusped boundaries (e.g., the Koch snowflake) are out of scope. `BoxRegion` and `BallRegion` both satisfy Lipschitz trivially.
- **No spatial-Chernoff-killing cross terms.** The current contract treats the inner Chernoff as a black box; an inner-aware killing wrapper that uses spatial information from $C$ to refine the indicator (e.g., partial-cell masking at $\partial R$) is deferred.
- **`apply_parallel_into` not shipped.** The v2.6 `KillingChernoff` post-multiply is single-threaded; parallelization is straightforward (per-cell independence) and may ship in a v2.6.x PATCH if benchmark evidence demands it.

### §21.7 — References

- N. V. Butko, *Approximation of subordinate semigroups by Chernoff iterations involving killing*, **Fract. Calc. Appl. Anal.** 21:5 (2018), pp. 1206–1228. doi:10.1515/fca-2018-0064. — Theorem 3.1 (Chernoff approximation of killed Feynman–Kac semigroups); §3.2 (order-1 truncation bound); §5 (open problem on higher-order killing).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — original Chernoff theorem (§2; cited in §2 of this document for the unrestricted case).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** (2025) — Theorem 6 (cited in §1 of this document); the killing wrapper preserves the Chernoff hypothesis under post-multiplication by an indicator (extension of Theorem 6 §3, straightforward).

### §21.8 — v7.0.0 NOTE — Order-2 via SOFT killing-RATE symmetric Strang (item #26, ADR-0126) (NORMATIVE library; PRE-FLIGHT-verified)

**Scope refinement (load-bearing).** Butko 2018 §5 conjectures order-2 killing via the symmetrization $\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}\,C(\tau)\,\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}$ (§21.6). A v7.0.0 PRE-FLIGHT (`scripts/verify_killing_order2_preflight.py`, executed 2026-06-05) establishes that **over the hard absorbing indicator $\mathbb{1}_R$ the conjecture is vacuous**: $\mathbb{1}_R$ is idempotent ($0^{1/2}=0$, $1^{1/2}=1$), so $\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2} = \mathbb{1}_R$ and the "symmetric split" degenerates to $\mathbb{1}_R\,C\,\mathbb{1}_R$ — whose *left* factor is exactly the **pre-multiply over-killing form §21.2 REJECTS**. The boundary discontinuity makes $[L, \mathbb{1}_R]$ an irreducible $O(\tau)$ term; the hard absorbing wall ($u|_{\partial R}=0$) is order-1, full stop. The v2.6 `KillingChernoff<C, R>` (§21.3) is UNCHANGED.

**The order-2 path — SOFT killing.** The conjecture has teeth only for a smooth bounded killing **rate** $\kappa(x) \ge 0$ (a reaction term $-\kappa u$; Feynman-Kac with continuous weight $e^{-\int_0^t \kappa(X_s)\,ds}$, killed generator $L_\kappa = L - \kappa$). There $R^{1/2}(\tau) := e^{-\tau\kappa/2}$ is a genuine non-idempotent multiplication factor, $[L,\kappa]$ is bounded (no boundary jump), and the palindrome
$$
S(\tau) \;:=\; e^{-\tau\kappa/2}\,C_L(\tau)\,e^{-\tau\kappa/2} \;=\; e^{\tau(L-\kappa)} + O(\tau^3)
$$
is **order-2 globally**. The PRE-FLIGHT confirms it on a faithful non-commuting model ($L = \tfrac12\,\text{discrete }\partial_{xx}$, $\kappa = \mathrm{diag}(0.3,0.7,0.2)$, $[L,\kappa]\neq 0$): the $\tau^1$ and $\tau^2$ coefficient matrices of $S(\tau)-e^{\tau(L-\kappa)}$ are exactly zero, $\tau^3$ nonzero (canonical Strang local $O(\tau^3) \Rightarrow$ global $O(\tau^2)$). v7.0.0 ships this as a **new** additive `Killing2ndChernoff<C, K, F>` parameterised by a killing-RATE field $\kappa(x) \ge 0$ (a `KillingRate<F>` trait), NOT by a `KillingRegion`. The constructor validates $\kappa \ge 0$ (a negative rate is mass creation, fail-closed `DomainViolation`). Gate `G_KILLING_ORDER2`: self-convergence slope $\le -1.95$ vs $e^{t(L-\kappa)}$.

**Honest cross-reference.** `Killing2ndChernoff` (continuous soft killing, order-2) and `KillingChernoff` (hard absorbing wall, order-1, §21.3) are DIFFERENT operators — not faster/slower versions of one. Users needing an absorbing Dirichlet boundary MUST use the order-1 §21 wrapper; `Killing2ndChernoff` does not solve the hard-wall problem at higher order (it cannot — §21.8 Para 1). Reference: Butko 2018 §5 (the rate-formulation reading of the open problem); Strang 1968 SIAM J. Numer. Anal. 5:3 (palindromic split).

---

## §22 — Laplace-Chernoff resolvent (v2.7, ADR-0069, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §22.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For a closed densely-defined operator $A$ generating a strongly continuous semigroup $\{S(t)\}_{t \ge 0}$ on a Banach space $X$ with growth bound $\omega$ (i.e., $\|S(t)\| \le M \exp(\omega t)$ for some $M \ge 1$), the **resolvent** at $\lambda \in \mathbb{C}$ with $\operatorname{Re}(\lambda) > \omega$ is the bounded linear operator
$$
R(\lambda; A) \;:=\; (\lambda I - A)^{-1} \;:\; X \to X.
$$
