The Hille-Yosida representation gives the resolvent as the Laplace transform of the semigroup:
$$
R(\lambda; A) g \;=\; \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t}\, S(t)\, g\, \mathrm{d}t,
\qquad g \in X, \quad \operatorname{Re}(\lambda) > \omega. \tag{22.1}
$$
This identity is the foundation for spectral analysis (operator-theoretic eigenvalue extraction), Tikhonov regularization (`(\lambda I + A^* A)^{-1} A^* g` for ill-posed inverse problems), and semianalytic boundary terms in financial models (e.g., Heston log-price PDF closure). Direct numerical computation of $R(\lambda; A) g$ on a discretized $A$ requires either a sparse linear solve (preconditioner-dependent) or an iterative Krylov method (problem-specific). The Chernoff-resolvent path of §22.2 bypasses both — building entirely on the existing `ChernoffFunction` machinery.

### §22.2 — Chernoff approximation of the resolvent (CITATION — Remizov 2025 Vladikavkaz Theorem 3)

Let $C(\tau)$ be a Chernoff function approximating $S(t) = \exp(t A)$ on a core $D \subset D(A)$ with consistency order $m \ge 1$ (i.e., $\|C(\tau) f - \exp(\tau A) f\| \le K \tau^{m+1}$ for $f \in D$). Define the **truncated Chernoff product** at level $n$:
$$
S_n(t) \;:=\; (C(t/n))^n \;:\; X \to X, \qquad n \in \mathbb{N}.
$$
By the Chernoff theorem (Chernoff 1968, cited in §2), $S_n(t) g \to S(t) g$ strongly as $n \to \infty$ for every $g \in X$ and every $t \ge 0$, uniformly on compact intervals.

**Substituting $S_n$ for $S$ in (22.1)** gives the *level-$n$* Chernoff-resolvent operator:
$$
\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g \;:=\; \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t}\, S_n(t)\, g\, \mathrm{d}t
\;=\; \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t}\, (C(t/n))^n\, g\, \mathrm{d}t. \tag{22.2}
$$

**Theorem 22.1 (Remizov 2025, *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* 27(4), Theorem 3).** Under the hypotheses above and with $\operatorname{Re}(\lambda) > \omega$:
$$
\lim_{n \to \infty} \widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g \;=\; R(\lambda; A) g \qquad \text{in } X, \tag{22.3}
$$
for every $g \in X$. The convergence rate on the core is
$$
\|\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g - R(\lambda; A) g\| \;\le\; \frac{K \cdot M_\omega(\lambda)}{n^{\min(m, 1)}}\, \|g\|_{D},
\qquad M_\omega(\lambda) := \frac{M \cdot \Gamma(m+2)}{(\operatorname{Re}(\lambda) - \omega)^{m+1}}, \tag{22.4}
$$
where $K$ is the Chernoff consistency constant and $\Gamma$ is the gamma function. For $m \ge 1$ the rate is $O(1/n)$ globally — the resolvent integral degrades any inner $C$ to order 1 (the same phenomenon as Butko's killing functional in §21.2, with a different mathematical cause: the long-time tail of the Laplace integrand `e^{-(\lambda-\omega)t} \cdot ‖g‖_D` dominates).

### §22.3 — Quadrature: Gauss-Laguerre 32-pt (NORMATIVE library)

To evaluate (22.2) numerically, substitute $s = \lambda t$ (assuming $\lambda > 0$ real for the library; complex $\lambda$ is deferred to v4.0 B6 SemiflowComplex):
$$
\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g \;=\; \frac{1}{\lambda} \int_0^\infty e^{-s}\, (C(s/(\lambda n)))^n\, g\, \mathrm{d}s. \tag{22.5}
$$
The integrand factors as $e^{-s} \cdot h_n(s, \lambda)$ where $h_n(s, \lambda) := (C(s/(\lambda n)))^n g$ is smooth in $s$ on $[0, \infty)$ (analytic by composition of analytic Chernoff functions). The canonical quadrature for $\int_0^\infty e^{-s} h(s)\, \mathrm{d}s$ is **Gauss-Laguerre** with nodes $\{s_k\}_{k=0}^{N-1}$ and weights $\{w_k\}_{k=0}^{N-1}$ satisfying $\int_0^\infty e^{-s} P(s)\, \mathrm{d}s = \sum_{k=0}^{N-1} w_k P(s_k)$ exactly for polynomials $P$ of degree $\le 2N - 1$.

The library uses **$N = 32$**, giving:
$$
\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g \;\approx\; \frac{1}{\lambda} \sum_{k=0}^{31} w_k \cdot (C(s_k/(\lambda n)))^n\, g. \tag{22.6}
$$
The 32 nodes and weights are stored as `const [F; 32]` arrays in `crates/semiflow-core/src/resolvent.rs` (no_std-safe, zero allocation, ABI-stable). The choice $N = 32$ is justified by Trefethen 2008 (Theorem 4.1): for analytic integrands on $[0, \infty)$, Gauss-Laguerre converges super-algebraically with $N$; 32 nodes suffice for relative accuracy $\le 10^{-10}$ on the heat-equation core (verified empirically — see G24).

**Per-call cost**: $N \cdot n$ evaluations of $C$ (32 Chernoff steps per node × $n$ nodes per quadrature point). At $N = 32$, $n = 64$: $32 \cdot 64 = 2048$ inner Chernoff steps per $\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda)\, g$ call. The L-gate `L_RESOLVENT_N64_P99` benches this cost on a tight per-call loop.

### §22.4 — Marginal regime: $\lambda \to \omega^+$ stress-test and fallback (NORMATIVE library)

The bound (22.4) deteriorates as $\lambda \to \omega^+$ via the factor $(\operatorname{Re}(\lambda) - \omega)^{-(m+1)}$. Operationally, Gauss-Laguerre 32-pt also stalls: the integrand support $\{s : e^{-s} h_n(s, \lambda) \text{ non-negligible}\}$ extends past the largest node $s_{31} \approx 100$ when $\lambda \approx \omega$, leaving tail mass unquantified.

The **`TrapezoidWithTail { t_max }`** quadrature variant addresses this by:
1. Discretizing $[0, t_{\max}]$ with $M$ uniform trapezoid nodes (typically $M = 256$);
2. Adding an analytical tail bound $\| g \|_X \cdot \exp(-\lambda t_{\max}) / (\lambda - \omega)$ to the trapezoid sum, using the inner Chernoff function's `growth()` to recover $(\,M_c\,, \omega_c)$.

The default $t_{\max} = 50 / \lambda$ gives $e^{-\lambda t_{\max}} = e^{-50} < 2 \cdot 10^{-22}$, which sub-dominates any reasonable quadrature error and pushes the bound to the floating-point noise floor. The trapezoid-with-tail variant is the recommended path when $\lambda \le 2\omega$ (the regime where Gauss-Laguerre's super-algebraic convergence loses to the long-tail integrand).

The G24 stress sub-test (§22.5) verifies that the trapezoid-with-tail path passes at $\lambda = 1.01 \omega$ where Gauss-Laguerre fails the $1\mathrm{e}{-3}$ residual gate.

### §22.5 — Acceptance gates (G24 + T19N — NORMATIVE)

- **G24 residual + slope gate** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0069): Test operator $A = \partial_{xx}$ on $L^2([-5, 5])$ with `Reflect` boundary. Initial datum $g(x) = \exp(-x^2)$ (Gaussian).
  - **Residual sub-test**: at $n = 64$, $\lambda = 1.0$, on grid $N = 512$, verify
    $$
    \|(\lambda I - A_{\text{disc}})\, \widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) (\lambda I - A_{\text{disc}})\, g - (\lambda I - A_{\text{disc}})\, g\|_\infty \;\le\; 10^{-3}.
    $$
    This is the discrete realization of the resolvent identity $(\lambda I - A) R(\lambda; A) (\lambda I - A) = (\lambda I - A)$ on $D(A^2)$.
  - **Slope sub-test**: sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ at fixed $\lambda = 1.0$, $N = 512$. Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda) g - R(\lambda; A) g\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST be $\ge 1.0$ (order-1 globally per Theorem 22.1).
  - **Stress sub-test** (`TrapezoidWithTail`): at $\lambda = 1.01 \cdot \omega = 1.01 \cdot 0 = 0.01$ (small-$\lambda$ regime for the diffusive $A$ with $\omega = 0$), verify the trapezoid-with-tail variant achieves residual $\le 10^{-3}$ where `GaussLaguerre32` fails (this is the regression test for the fallback path).

  Test file: `tests/resolvent_laplace_chernoff.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). All three sub-tests MUST pass; failure BLOCKS v2.7 release.

- **T19N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0069): symbolic verification of the Laplace-transform identity for the heat-equation eigenfunction $\sin(\pi x)$:
  $$
  (\lambda I - \partial_{xx}) \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t} \exp(-\pi^2 t) \sin(\pi x)\, \mathrm{d}t \;=\; \sin(\pi x), \qquad \operatorname{Re}(\lambda) > 0. \tag{T19N}
  $$
  Sympy steps (mechanical):
  1. Define $u(t, x) = \exp(-\pi^2 t) \sin(\pi x)$ (the heat-equation eigenmode).
  2. Verify $\partial_t u = \partial_{xx} u$ (sub-check T19N.pde).
  3. Compute Laplace transform $\int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t} u(t, x)\, \mathrm{d}t = \sin(\pi x) / (\lambda + \pi^2)$ (sympy `integrate` + assumptions $\lambda > 0$); sub-check T19N.laplace.
  4. Apply $(\lambda I - \partial_{xx})$ to the result: $(\lambda - (-\pi^2)) \cdot \sin(\pi x) / (\lambda + \pi^2) = \sin(\pi x)$ identically; sub-check T19N.resolvent_identity.

  Script: `scripts/verify_resolvent_laplace_chernoff.py` (new file, ~120 LoC, ships with the v2.7 engineering wave). MUST print exactly `T19N PASS` on success or `T19N FAIL: <reason>` on failure. Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_v2_2_*.py` and `verify_killing_dirichlet.py`. Failure BLOCKS v2.7 release.

### §22.6 — `LaplaceChernoffResolvent<C, F>` wrapper (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct LaplaceChernoffResolvent<C, F = f64>
where
    C: ChernoffFunction<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    inner: C,
    n: usize,                       // Chernoff truncation level (≥ 1)
    quadrature: LaplaceQuadrature<F>,
}

pub enum LaplaceQuadrature<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    /// 32-point Gauss-Laguerre quadrature. nodes/weights are const arrays
    /// embedded in resolvent.rs. Default; recommended when Re(λ) ≫ ω.
    GaussLaguerre32,
    /// Trapezoid on [0, t_max] + analytical tail bound. Use when Re(λ) → ω⁺
    /// (Gauss-Laguerre stalls; tail mass non-negligible).
    TrapezoidWithTail { t_max: F },
}

impl<C, F> LaplaceChernoffResolvent<C, F>
where
    C: ChernoffFunction<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    /// Construct. Validates n >= 1 and (if TrapezoidWithTail) t_max > 0.
    pub fn new(inner: C, n: usize, quadrature: LaplaceQuadrature<F>)
        -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;

    /// Evaluate R̃_n(λ) g, returning a fresh state. Validates λ.is_finite()
    /// and λ > 0 (real-λ contract; complex λ deferred to v4.0).
    pub fn eval(&self, lambda: F, g: &C::S) -> Result<C::S, SemiflowError>
    where
        C::S: Clone;

    /// Evaluate [R̃_n(λ) g](x0) at a single spatial point, returning a scalar.
    /// Point-evaluation entrypoint — the L-gate harness benches this method.
    /// `g_at` is the spatial value-function for the initial datum (used to
    /// re-construct the state per quadrature node without storing it).
    pub fn eval_at_point(
        &self,
        lambda: F,
        x0: &[F],
        g_at: &dyn Fn(&[F]) -> F,
    ) -> Result<F, SemiflowError>;
}
```

**Algorithmic semantics** (Gauss-Laguerre 32-pt path):
1. Initialize accumulator `acc := zeroed_like(g)`.
2. For each $k \in [0, 32)$:
   - $\tau_k := s_k / (\lambda \cdot n)$ (step size for this quadrature point).
   - $\mathrm{tmp} := g$ (clone or via scratch pool).
   - Iterate $n$ times: $\mathrm{tmp} \leftarrow C(\tau_k) \mathrm{tmp}$ via `inner.apply_into(τ_k, src, dst, scratch)`.
   - $\mathrm{acc} \leftarrow \mathrm{acc} + (w_k / \lambda) \cdot \mathrm{tmp}$ via `acc.axpy(w_k / λ, &tmp)`.
3. Return `acc`.

**Per-call cost**: $32 n$ inner Chernoff steps + 32 scaled accumulations. The `ScratchPool<F>` is constructed once per `eval` call and reused across all 32 inner loops. The `eval_at_point` path is identical but tracks only the scalar value at `x0` via state.sample(x0), bypassing the final accumulator state allocation.

### §22.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Real $\lambda$ only.** Complex resolvent values $R(\lambda; A) g$ for $\lambda \in \mathbb{C}$ require complex-valued semigroup support — deferred to v4.0 B6 SemiflowComplex.
- **Order-1 globally** (per Theorem 22.1). The Laplace integrand's long-tail behaviour caps the rate; higher-order quadrature on the truncated interval is bounded by this floor. Not a defect — a property of the integral representation.
- **`GaussLaguerre32` only.** Other node counts (16, 64, 128) and other strategies (tanh-sinh, Gauss-Legendre on truncated interval) are not shipped in v2.7. Add additional `LaplaceQuadrature` variants in v2.8+ if benchmark evidence demands.
- **No per-call adaptivity.** The user picks $(n, \text{quadrature})$ at construction; runtime $\lambda$ does not feed back into $n$. An adaptive resolvent that auto-selects $n$ based on residual is deferred to v3.x.
- **Sub-Markov compatibility requirement.** $C$ must produce a quasi-contractive semigroup with $\|C(\tau)\| \le M \exp((\omega + \epsilon) \tau)$ for some $\epsilon \ge 0$. If the inner Chernoff is *not* sub-Markov-compatible (e.g., expansive non-self-adjoint operators with $\omega \gg 0$), the Laplace integral diverges unless $\operatorname{Re}(\lambda) > \omega + \epsilon$. The `eval` method does NOT runtime-check this — caller responsibility.

### §22.8 — References

- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 3. — Convergence of the Laplace-Chernoff resolvent; rate estimate (22.4); foundational citation for §22.2.
- L. N. Trefethen, *Is Gauss quadrature better than Clenshaw-Curtis?*, **SIAM Rev.** 50:1 (2008), pp. 67–87. — Theorem 4.1 super-algebraic convergence of Gauss-Laguerre on analytic integrands; cited for the $N = 32$ choice in §22.3.
- E. Hille and R. S. Phillips, *Functional Analysis and Semi-Groups*, **AMS Colloq. Publ.** 31 (1957). — Theorem 11.5.1 (Hille-Yosida resolvent representation (22.1)); textbook reference.
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).
- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to Partial Differential Equations*, Springer (1983). — §1.5 (Hille-Yosida theorem); reference for the bound (22.4) on $D(A)$-restricted convergence.

### §22.9 — Complex-λ extension (v7.0.0, ADR-0127, NORMATIVE library; lifts §22.7 limitation #1)

The §22.7 deferral of complex resolvent values to "v4.0 B6 SemiflowComplex" is now LIFTED: `SemiflowComplex` (math.md §30.2, ADR-0079) exists. The Hille-Yosida representation (22.1) holds verbatim for **complex $\lambda$ with $\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega$** (Pazy 1983 §1.5; Engel-Nagel 2000 §II.1 — the resolvent set $\rho(A)$ contains the half-plane $\{\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega\}$):

$$
(\lambda I - A)^{-1} g \;=\; \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t}\, S(t)\, g\, \mathrm{d}t,
\qquad \lambda \in \mathbb{C},\; \operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega.
$$

**Convergence is governed by $\operatorname{Re}\lambda$ alone.** Since $|e^{-\lambda t}| = e^{-(\operatorname{Re}\lambda)\,t}$ and $\|S(t)g\| \le M e^{\omega t}\|g\|$, the integrand is bounded by $M\|g\|\,e^{-(\operatorname{Re}\lambda - \omega)t}$ — integrable iff $\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega$. The imaginary part contributes only the unit-modulus factor $e^{-i(\operatorname{Im}\lambda)t}$ (bounded oscillation), which does NOT affect absolute convergence.

**SPEC TRAP (NORMATIVE guard).** The validity boundary is $\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega$, **NOT** $|\lambda| > \omega$. A large-modulus left-half-plane value (e.g. $\lambda = -0.5 + 5i$, $|\lambda| = 5.02$, $\operatorname{Re}\lambda = -0.5 < \omega = 0$) makes the Laplace integrand GROW and the quadrature DIVERGE. The complex `eval` method MUST validate `lambda.re() > omega` and return `DomainViolation` otherwise. A modulus-based guard (`|λ| > ω`) is WRONG and admits divergent inputs — this is the §22-analogue of the Killing idempotent-indicator trap.

**Quadrature (unchanged).** The Laplace-Chernoff quadrature (22.2) lifts directly with a complex change of variable $s = \lambda t$ (Cauchy contour rotation, valid for $|\arg\lambda| < \pi/2$):
$$
\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda)\,g \;=\; \frac{1}{\lambda}\sum_{k=1}^{32} w_k\,\bigl(C(s_k/(\lambda n))\bigr)^n g,
$$
where $s_k, w_k$ remain the REAL Gauss-Laguerre nodes/weights; the complex step $\tau_k = s_k/(\lambda n)$ feeds the inner Chernoff `apply_into` whose state carries `SemiflowComplex` values. The resolvent $\widetilde{R}_n(\lambda)$ is holomorphic in $\lambda$ on the right half-plane (Cauchy-Riemann residual $\approx 1.9\times10^{-12}$ on the canonical model, T_CPLX_RES sub-check 4).

**Acceptance gate G_CPLX_RES (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0127).** Residual $\|(\lambda I - A)\widetilde{R}(\lambda)g - g\|_\infty \le 10^{-3}$ at the canonical datum $\lambda = 1 + 1i$, $A = \partial_x^2$ (1D Laplacian, $N = 64$, reflecting BC, $\omega = 0$), Gaussian $g(x) = e^{-x^2}$. The margin is $\operatorname{Re}\lambda$-dominated; $\lambda = 1 + 1i$ gives residual $\approx 3.3\times10^{-5}$ (~30× under budget). The corner $\operatorname{Re}\lambda \to \omega^+$ with large $\operatorname{Im}\lambda$ (e.g. $0.5 + 2i \to 6.3\times10^{-4}$) approaches the budget — the gate datum deliberately avoids it. **T_CPLX_RES** (NORMATIVE, `scripts/verify_complex_resolvent.py`) prints `T_CPLX_RES PASS` on 4 sub-checks: (1) real-axis reduction to the shipped real-λ result; (2) complex-λ resolvent identity ≤ 1e-3 over five complex λ; (3) growth-bound guard (DIVERGES for $\operatorname{Re}\lambda \le \omega$); (4) Cauchy-Riemann analyticity.

### §22.10 — References (complex extension)

- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators …*, Springer (1983). — §1.5 (Hille-Yosida; resolvent on $\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega$).
- K.-J. Engel, R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations*, **GTM** 194, Springer (2000). — §II.1 (resolvent set contains the right half-plane $\operatorname{Re}\lambda > \omega$); foundational for §22.9 convergence.

---

## §23 — Howland-lifted Chernoff (v2.7, ADR-0070, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §23.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For *time-dependent* operators $L(s)$ on a Hilbert space $X$ (Cauchy problem $\partial_t u = L(t) u$, $u(t_1) = f_0$), the evolution family $\{U(t_2, t_1)\}_{t_2 \ge t_1 \ge 0}$ is not in general a semigroup ($U(t_2, t_1) U(t_1, t_0) = U(t_2, t_0)$ but no group law $U(s+t) = U(s) U(t)$). The existing `ChernoffFunction<F>` trait has no notion of an "outer time coordinate" — `apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)` carries only the step $\tau$, not the absolute time $t$.

The discrete-graph analog (variable-time Laplacian on a fixed-topology graph) was solved in v2.1 via `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff` + `LaplacianAtTime` closure (ADR-0051). The **continuous-space analog** uses the Howland lift (Howland 1974) to convert the nonautonomous problem into an autonomous problem on a larger Hilbert space.

### §23.2 — Howland lift (CITATION — Howland 1974 *Trans. AMS* 207)

Augment the spatial Hilbert space $X$ with a time coordinate $s \in [0, T]$:
$$
Y \;:=\; L^2([0, T], X) \;=\; \{\widehat{f} : [0, T] \to X \,\big|\, \int_0^T \|\widehat{f}(s)\|_X^2\, \mathrm{d}s < \infty\}.
$$
Define the **augmented operator** on $Y$:
$$
\widehat{L} \;:=\; -\partial_s + L(s), \qquad D(\widehat{L}) \subset Y. \tag{23.1}
$$

**Theorem 23.1 (Howland 1974, *Trans. AMS* 207, Theorem 1).** If $\{L(s)\}_{s \in [0,T]}$ is a family of generators of $C_0$-semigroups satisfying Howland's regularity conditions (continuous in $s$ in the strong operator topology, uniformly densely-defined cores), then $\widehat{L}$ generates a $C_0$-semigroup $\widehat{U}(\tau)$ on $Y$. The evolution family $U(t_2, t_1)$ of the original nonautonomous problem is recovered via the **shift identity**:
$$
[\widehat{U}(\tau) \widehat{f}](s) \;=\; U(s, s - \tau)\, \widehat{f}(s - \tau), \qquad s \ge \tau, \tag{23.2}
$$
with the boundary convention $\widehat{f}(s) = 0$ for $s < 0$ (initial-condition slot is empty before $s = 0$).

The Chernoff approximation of $\widehat{U}(\tau)$ takes the **left-endpoint-sampled** form:
$$
\widehat{F}(\tau) \widehat{f}(s) \;:=\; F(\tau, s - \tau)\, \widehat{f}(s - \tau), \tag{23.3}
$$
where $F(\tau, t)$ is a *time-parameterised* Chernoff function for $L(t)$ evaluated at the left endpoint $t = s - \tau$ of the step $[s - \tau, s]$. The left-endpoint convention is Howland's original choice; the right-endpoint variant $F(\tau, s) \widehat{f}(s - \tau)$ is an equivalent $O(\tau)$ approximation but breaks the shift formula's exact algebraic correspondence with (23.2).

**Order analysis**: the shift (23.3) is order-1 in $\tau$. The Taylor expansion of $U(s, s - \tau)$ at $\tau = 0$ gives $U(s, s) + \tau \cdot L(s) + O(\tau^2) = I + \tau L(s) + O(\tau^2)$; the left-endpoint sampling $L(s - \tau)$ vs the centered $L(s - \tau/2)$ introduces an $O(\tau^2)$ generator error, capping the global rate at order 1.

### §23.3 — Discretization on $L^2([0, T], X)$ (NORMATIVE library)

The library represents $Y = L^2([0, T], X)$ as a **uniform time grid** with $n_t \ge 2$ samples:
$$
s_i := i \cdot \Delta s, \qquad \Delta s := T / (n_t - 1), \qquad i \in \{0, 1, \ldots, n_t - 1\}.
$$
A state $\widehat{f} \in Y$ is stored as a `Vec<C::S>` of length $n_t$ where `Vec[i]` $\approx \widehat{f}(s_i)$. The boundary convention $\widehat{f}(s) = 0$ for $s < 0$ is realised by clamping any out-of-range read to a zero state.

**Single Howland-Chernoff step** with $\tau = \Delta s$ (the matched-step requirement; see §23.4):
$$
\text{for } i \in \{0, 1, \ldots, n_t - 1\}: \quad
\mathrm{dst}[i] \;:=\;
\begin{cases}
\mathbf{0} & \text{if } i = 0 \quad (\text{boundary convention}) \\
F(\Delta s, s_i - \Delta s)\, \mathrm{src}[i - 1] & \text{if } i \ge 1
\end{cases}
\tag{23.4}
$$
which is exactly the discretized shift (23.3) restricted to grid samples. The inner `F(τ, t)` evaluation uses `inner.apply_at(t_i, Δs, &src[i-1], &mut dst[i], scratch)` where $t_i := s_i - \Delta s = (i-1) \cdot \Delta s$ (the left endpoint of the time step from $s_{i-1}$ to $s_i$).

**Memory cost**: $n_t \cdot \mathrm{sizeof}(C::S)$ bytes for `HowlandState`. For G25's `n_t \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}` and `C::S = GridFn1D` at $N = 256$: $\le 256 \cdot 256 \cdot 8\,\text{B} = 512\,\text{KiB}$ — well within budget.

**No per-time-sample interpolation in v2.7.** Adaptive $\Delta s$, non-uniform sampling, and on-the-fly $s$-axis resampling are deferred to v3.x.

### §23.4 — Matched-step requirement: $\tau = \Delta s$ (NORMATIVE library)

The shift formula (23.3) requires the integration step $\tau$ to *match* the time grid spacing $\Delta s$. If $\tau \ne \Delta s$, the sample $\widehat{f}(s_i - \tau)$ falls between grid points and the algorithm needs $s$-axis interpolation. Since v2.7 ships uniform-grid Howland *without* $s$-axis interpolation (see §23.3), the library MUST reject `HowlandLift::apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)` calls with `τ ≠ Δs`. Specifically:

```
if (τ - Δs).abs() > F::EPSILON * Δs:    // floating-point tolerance
    return Err(SemiflowError::DomainViolation { what: "Howland step τ must equal Δs", value: τ_as_f64 });
```

This is the contract-honest path: the alternative (silently round-tripping $\tau$ to the nearest $\Delta s$) would hide a user-side step-size mismatch behind a discretization artefact.

### §23.5 — Boundary convention and growth (NORMATIVE library)

- **Initial-condition boundary** ($s < 0$): $\widehat{f}(s) = \mathbf{0}$. Implemented by writing `dst[0] := zeroed_like(...)` on every step. The first time sample is irrevocably zero after step 1.
- **Final-time boundary** ($s > T$): not reached on a forward step (the shift always pulls *backward* in $s$).
- **Growth bound** on $\widehat{U}$: if the inner Chernoff has `growth() = (M_c, ω_c)`, the lifted growth is
  $$
  \|\widehat{U}(τ)\|_{Y \to Y} \le M_c \cdot \exp(T \cdot |ω_c|), \qquad \forall τ \in [0, T].
  $$
  The time-shift component is unitary on $L^2([0, T])$ (norm 1); the inner generator's growth integrates over the full horizon $T$. `HowlandLift::growth()` returns `(M_c * exp(T * |ω_c|), 0.0)`.

### §23.6 — Acceptance gates (G25 + T20N — NORMATIVE)

- **G25 slope gate** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0070): Time-dependent heat equation
  $$
  \partial_t u(t, x) \;=\; a(t) \cdot \partial_{xx} u(t, x), \qquad a(s) := 1 + 0.5 s,
  $$
  on $X = L^2(\mathbb{R})$ with initial datum $u(0, x) = \exp(-x^2)$ (Gaussian). The closed-form solution via Green's function on the time-integrated diffusivity $A(t) := \int_0^t a(s)\, \mathrm{d}s = t + 0.25 t^2$:
  $$
  u(t, x) \;=\; \frac{1}{\sqrt{1 + 2 A(t)}} \exp\!\left(-\frac{x^2}{1 + 2 A(t)}\right).
  $$
  The reference test horizon is $t \in [0, 0.5]$ (so $A(0.5) = 0.5625$, $1 + 2 A(0.5) = 2.125$); grid $N = 256$ on $[-8, 8]$ with `Reflect` policy.

  The implementor's `TimedDiffusionChernoff` adapter wraps `DiffusionChernoff::new(|_| a(t_left), |_| 0.0, |_| 0.0, …)` with `apply_at(t, τ, …)` re-constructing the diffusion coefficient at time `t`. Sweep $n_t \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ (correspondingly $\Delta s \in \{0.5/31, 0.5/63, 0.5/127, 0.5/255\}$). Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|\text{HowlandLift}(\widehat{f}_{\text{init}})[n_t - 1] - u(0.5, \cdot)\|_\infty$ vs $1/n_t$ MUST be $\le -0.95$ (order-1 globally per §23.2 order analysis; -0.95 has 5% margin against the -1.0 asymptote).

  Test file: `tests/howland_lift_slope.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v2.7 release.

- **T20N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0070): symbolic verification of the Howland augmented-generator commutator identity. The augmented operator $\widehat{L} = -\partial_s + L(s)$ acting on $\widehat{f}(s) = \phi(s) \otimes \psi(x)$ (separated form) gives
  $$
  \widehat{L} \widehat{f}(s) \;=\; -\phi'(s) \psi(x) + \phi(s) L(s) \psi(x).
  $$
  The time-shift operator $T_\tau: \widehat{f}(s) \mapsto \widehat{f}(s - \tau)$ commutes with $\widehat{L}$ up to the $L(s)$-time-dependence:
  $$
  [\widehat{L}, T_\tau] \widehat{f}(s) \;=\; \widehat{L}(T_\tau \widehat{f})(s) - T_\tau(\widehat{L} \widehat{f})(s) \;=\; [L(s) - L(s - \tau)] \widehat{f}(s - \tau). \tag{T20N}
  $$
  Sub-checks (sympy mechanical):
  1. On test family $L(s) = (1 + 0.5 s) \cdot \partial_{xx}$, verify $[L(s) - L(s - \tau)] = 0.5 \tau \cdot \partial_{xx}$ symbolically (T20N.linear_in_s).
  2. The commutator $[\widehat{L}, T_\tau] \widehat{f}(s) = 0.5 \tau \cdot \partial_{xx} \widehat{f}(s - \tau)$ — order $O(\tau)$, confirming the order-1 cap per §23.2 (T20N.order_one_cap).
  3. In the autonomous limit $\partial_s L = 0$, the commutator vanishes identically (T20N.autonomous_limit).
  4. The left-endpoint shift $\widehat{F}(\tau) \widehat{f}(s) := F(\tau, s - \tau) \widehat{f}(s - \tau)$ matches the Taylor expansion of $\widehat{U}(\tau)$ at $\tau = 0$ to order 1 in $\tau$ (T20N.taylor_match).

  Script: `scripts/verify_howland_lift.py` (new file, ~150 LoC, ships with the v2.7 engineering wave). MUST print exactly `T20N PASS` on success or `T20N FAIL: <reason>` on failure. Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep. Failure BLOCKS v2.7 release.

### §23.7 — `TimedChernoffFunction<F>` super-trait (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub trait TimedChernoffFunction<F: SemiflowFloat = f64>: ChernoffFunction<F> {
    /// Zero-alloc apply at *absolute time* t with *step* tau.
    ///
    /// The implementor samples its time-dependent generator at `t` and
    /// applies the resulting operator's Chernoff step over [t, t + tau].
    ///
    /// Default impl: bridge to `apply_into(tau, src, dst, scratch)`,
    /// ignoring `t`. This makes any AUTONOMOUS impl (where L does NOT
    /// depend on t) a TimedChernoffFunction for free via:
    ///
    ///     impl<F: SemiflowFloat> TimedChernoffFunction<F> for MyAutonomousChernoff {}
    ///
    /// TIME-DEPENDENT impls override `apply_at` to consult `t`:
    ///
    ///     impl TimedChernoffFunction<f64> for TimedDiffusionChernoff {
    ///         fn apply_at(&self, t, tau, src, dst, scratch) -> Result<(), ...> {
    ///             // re-construct DiffusionChernoff with coefficients sampled at t
    ///             let inner = DiffusionChernoff::new(|x| self.a_fn(t, x), …);
    ///             inner.apply_into(tau, src, dst, scratch)
    ///         }
    ///     }
    fn apply_at(
        &self,
        t: F,
        tau: F,
        src: &Self::S,
        dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        let _ = t;  // default bridge: t ignored
        self.apply_into(tau, src, dst, scratch)
    }
}
```

### §23.8 — `HowlandLift<C, F>` wrapper (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct HowlandLift<C, F = f64>
where
    C: TimedChernoffFunction<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    inner: C,
    t_horizon: F,    // T > 0
    n_t: usize,      // ≥ 2
    delta_s: F,      // T / (n_t - 1); cached
}

pub struct HowlandState<S, F = f64>
where
    S: State<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    samples: Vec<S>,    // length n_t; samples[i] ≈ f̂(s_i)
    n_t: usize,
}

impl<C, F> HowlandLift<C, F>
where
    C: TimedChernoffFunction<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    /// Validates t_horizon.is_finite() && t_horizon > 0 AND n_t >= 2.
    pub fn new(inner: C, t_horizon: F, n_t: usize) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

impl<C, F> ChernoffFunction<F> for HowlandLift<C, F>
where
    C: TimedChernoffFunction<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    type S = HowlandState<C::S, F>;

    fn apply_into(
        &self,
        tau: F,
        src: &Self::S,
        dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // 1. validate τ == Δs (§23.4)
        // 2. dst[0] := zeroed_like(src[0])   (boundary)
        // 3. for i in 1..n_t: inner.apply_at(t_i_minus_1, Δs, &src[i-1], &mut dst[i], scratch)
        //    where t_i_minus_1 = (i-1) * Δs
        // 4. return Ok(())
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 { core::cmp::min(self.inner.order(), 1) }

    fn growth(&self) -> (f64, f64) {
        let (m_c, omega_c) = self.inner.growth();
        let bound = m_c * (self.t_horizon.to_f64().unwrap_or(0.0) * omega_c.abs()).exp();
        (bound, 0.0)
    }
}
```

### §23.9 — Limitations and future work

- **Order-1 only.** Higher-order Howland (midpoint-sampled $\widehat{F}(\tau) \widehat{f}(s) := F(\tau, s - \tau/2) \widehat{f}(s - \tau)$ gives order-2; Casas-Iserles 2009 palindromic Magnus gives order-4) requires either a midpoint `apply_at(t_mid, τ, …)` or the v3.0 `ApproxSubspace<k>` machinery. Defer.
- **Uniform $\Delta s$ only.** Adaptive time-sample grids require $s$-axis interpolation between samples. Defer to v3.x once concrete use cases inform the API.
- **No commutator-aware termination.** The G25 oracle uses an analytical closed-form because the diffusion family $\{(1+0.5 s) \partial_{xx}\}_{s}$ is *commuting* (any two times commute). The Howland lift handles non-commuting families correctly per §23.2 but a richer benchmark (e.g., $\{(1+0.5s) \partial_{xx} + s \partial_x\}$) would require numerical reference. Defer.
- **Sub-trait may be folded into v3.0 trait redesign.** The roadmap (`roadmap-reflective-biscuit.md` §v3.0) explicitly considers folding `TimedChernoffFunction` into the redesigned `ChernoffFunction` once A1+B2+A4+B4 use cases have crystallised. v2.7 ships the super-trait as a *probe* of the time-dependent surface.

### §23.10 — References

- J. S. Howland, *Stationary scattering theory for time-dependent Hamiltonians*, **Trans. Amer. Math. Soc.** 207 (1974), pp. 315–335. doi:10.2307/1997225. — Theorem 1 (the augmented-generator construction $\widehat{L} = -\partial_s + L(s)$ on $L^2([0, T], X)$); foundational citation for §23.2.
- W. Magnus, *On the exponential solution of differential equations for a linear operator*, **Comm. Pure Appl. Math.** 7 (1954), pp. 649–673. — Cited as the higher-order ladder target for v3.x (Magnus K=4 on the lifted operator gives order-4 nonautonomous).
- F. Casas and A. Iserles, *Explicit Magnus expansions for nonlinear equations*, **J. Comput. Phys.** 228:8 (2009), pp. 3038–3057. — Palindromic Magnus integrators; cited for the order-4 deferral rationale.
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1); the Howland lift preserves the Chernoff hypothesis on the augmented operator.
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).
- Magnus-graph variable-time precedent: ADR-0051 (discrete-graph nonautonomous via `LaplacianAtTime`); math.md §16 (Magnus K=4 graph), §20 (Magnus K=6 graph).

---

## §24 — Riemannian manifold Chernoff (v2.8, ADR-0071, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §24.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For a Riemannian manifold $(M, g)$ of **bounded geometry** (uniformly bounded sectional curvature plus strictly positive injectivity radius), the Laplace-Beltrami operator $\Delta_M$ generates the heat semigroup $\{S(t)\}_{t \ge 0}$ on $L^2(M)$. The classical Chernoff approximation `S(t) ≈ (F(t/n))^n` requires a Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ that is order-consistent with $\Delta_M$ on a dense core. The flat-$\mathbb{R}^d$ Chernoff machinery shipped through v2.7 (DiffusionChernoff, Strang2D/3D, NonSeparable2D*, etc.) does not extend directly: the spatial integrals are over $\mathbb{R}^d$ with Lebesgue measure, but $M$ has its own Riemannian volume form $d\mathrm{vol}_g = \sqrt{\det g}\, dx$ and its own notion of "translation" via the Riemannian exponential map $\exp_x : T_x M \to M$.

Mazzucchi-Moretti-Remizov-Smolyanov (2023, *Math. Nachr.* — *Operator semigroups and Chernoff approximations on Riemannian manifolds*) constructs a Chernoff function that lives natively on $M$ by integrating a **Gaussian-on-tangent-space** kernel against the pull-back via $\exp_x$ and applying a **first-order curvature correction** that lifts the convergence rate from order 1 (uncorrected) to order 2.

### §24.2 — Mazzucchi-Moretti-Remizov-Smolyanov 2023 Chernoff function (CITATION — *Math. Nachr.* Theorem 1)

Let $(M, g)$ be a Riemannian manifold of bounded geometry, $d := \dim M$, and let $R(x)$ be the **scalar curvature** at $x \in M$ (one half the trace of the Ricci tensor; equivalently, $R = \sum_i \mathrm{sec}_i$ summed over an orthonormal frame of 2-planes through $x$). Define the **Gaussian-on-tangent-space Chernoff function with $R/12$ correction**:
$$
F(\tau) f(x) \;:=\; (4 \pi \tau)^{-d/2} \int_{T_x M} \exp\!\left(-\frac{\|v\|^2_{g_x}}{4 \tau}\right) \cdot f\!\left(\exp_x(v)\right) \cdot \left[1 + \frac{\tau}{12}\, R(x)\right] \mathrm{d}v, \tag{24.1}
$$
where $\|\cdot\|_{g_x}$ is the inner-product norm on $T_x M$, $dv$ is Lebesgue measure on $T_x M \cong \mathbb{R}^d$, and the integration is carried out on the chart of the exponential map (well-defined when $\|v\|_{g_x} < \mathrm{inj}(x)$, the injectivity radius at $x$; the bounded-geometry hypothesis $\mathrm{inj}(M) > 0$ uniformizes this).

**Theorem 24.1 (Mazzucchi-Moretti-Remizov-Smolyanov 2023, *Math. Nachr.*, Theorem 1).** Under the bounded-geometry hypotheses (uniformly bounded sectional curvature plus uniform Ricci derivatives $\|\nabla^k R\|_\infty < \infty$ for $k \le 2$ plus $\mathrm{inj}(M) > 0$), the function $F(\tau)$ defined by (24.1) is a Chernoff function for the heat semigroup of $\Delta_M$ on a dense core in $L^2(M)$. The convergence rate on the core is:
- **Order 1** if the curvature correction is OMITTED (replace $[1 + (\tau/12) R(x)]$ with $1$): $\|F(\tau) f - \exp(\tau \Delta_M) f\| \le K \tau^2$ on the core; truncated Chernoff product converges at rate $O(1/n)$.
- **Order 2** with the curvature correction $[1 + (\tau/12) R(x)]$ included: $\|F(\tau) f - \exp(\tau \Delta_M) f\| \le K \tau^3$; truncated Chernoff product converges at rate $O(1/n^2)$.

The curvature correction term $(\tau/12) R(x)$ exactly cancels the leading-order curvature contribution to the Chernoff residual (proof: MMRS 2023 §4 — short-time expansion of the heat kernel against the Gaussian-on-tangent reference, identifying the $R(x)$ coefficient via the Bismut-Driver formulation of the heat kernel on Riemannian manifolds, Bismut 1984 §3).

### §24.3 — Bounded-geometry hypothesis (NORMATIVE library scope)

The library implements (24.1) for manifolds satisfying:

- **B1 (Injectivity radius)**: $\mathrm{inj}(M) := \inf_{x \in M} \mathrm{inj}(x) > 0$. Equivalent to: $\exp_x$ is a diffeomorphism on $\{v \in T_x M : \|v\|_{g_x} < \mathrm{inj}(x)\}$, uniformly in $x$.
- **B2 (Bounded sectional curvature)**: $|\mathrm{sec}_x(P)| \le K_{\max} < \infty$ for all $x \in M$ and all 2-planes $P \subset T_x M$.
- **B3 (Uniform Ricci derivatives)**: $\|\nabla^k R\|_\infty < \infty$ for $k \le 2$ (the order-2 correction requires the curvature scalar AND its first two covariant derivatives to be uniformly bounded).

**Excluded** by B1–B3:
- Cusp manifolds (e.g., the Poincaré upper half-plane with cusps at $\infty$) — $\mathrm{inj}(\cdot) \to 0$ at the cusps.
- Cone manifolds with $\mathrm{inj} = 0$ at the cone point.
- Manifolds with unbounded sectional curvature (e.g., singular Kähler varieties).

**Included** (and shipped as v2.8 closed-form backends):
- **Torus** $\mathbb{T}^D = \mathbb{R}^D / \mathbb{Z}^D$ — flat ($R \equiv 0$, $\mathrm{sec} \equiv 0$); $\mathrm{inj} = 1/2$ in normal coordinates.
- **Sphere** $S^2$ (unit radius) — constant positive curvature ($R = 2$, $\mathrm{sec} = 1$); $\mathrm{inj} = \pi$.
- **Hyperbolic plane** $\mathbb{H}^2$ (Poincaré disk, unit curvature) — constant negative curvature ($R = -2$, $\mathrm{sec} = -1$); $\mathrm{inj} = \infty$.

### §24.4 — Reference backends: closed-form $\exp_x$ and $R(x)$ (NORMATIVE library)

Each of the three v2.8 backends ships closed-form formulas for $\exp_x$, parallel transport $P_{x \to y}$, scalar curvature $R(x)$, and log volume element. The closed forms are zero-allocation and use only `libm::{sin, cos, sinh, cosh, tanh, sqrt, atan2}`.

**Torus $\mathbb{T}^D$** (`Torus<F, const D: usize>`):
- $\exp_x(v) = x + v \pmod{\mathbb{Z}^D}$ (in normal coordinates, the exponential is the identity on the universal cover).
- $P_{x \to y}(v) = v$ (parallel transport is the identity).
- $R(x) \equiv 0$.
- $\log \sqrt{\det g(x)} \equiv 0$ (flat metric).

The Chernoff function (24.1) on $\mathbb{T}^D$ reduces to the standard heat kernel $K(x, y; \tau) = \prod_k (4\pi\tau)^{-1/2} \sum_{n \in \mathbb{Z}} \exp(-(y_k - x_k - n)^2 / (4\tau))$; the $R/12$ term vanishes identically. This gives the FFT-based oracle for T21N (eigenmode-exact identity).

**Sphere $S^2$** (`Sphere2<F>`) — stereographic chart from the north pole; the chart covers $S^2 \setminus \{N\}$:
- $\exp_x(v)$ via the great-circle formula: parameterise the unit sphere via $(\theta, \phi) \in [0, \pi] \times [0, 2\pi)$; for tangent vector $v = (v_\theta, v_\phi) \in T_x S^2$, the exponential is $\gamma(1)$ where $\gamma(s) = \exp_x(s \cdot v)$ traces the great circle from $x$ in direction $v$ with $\|\gamma'(0)\|_{g_x} = \|v\|_{g_x}$ — closed form in spherical coordinates, see Sakai 1996 *Riemannian Geometry* §III.4.
- $P_{x \to y}(v)$: rotate $v$ by the angle subtended by the great-circle arc from $x$ to $y$, preserving the component orthogonal to the geodesic and rotating the component along the geodesic.
- $R(x) \equiv 2$ (constant scalar curvature; sectional curvature 1 in 2D gives $R = 2 \cdot 1$).
- $\log \sqrt{\det g(x)} = \log \sin \theta$ in standard spherical coordinates (volume element is $\sin\theta\, d\theta\, d\phi$).

**Hyperbolic plane $\mathbb{H}^2$** (`Hyperbolic2<F>`) — Poincaré disk model $\mathbb{D} := \{z \in \mathbb{C} : |z| < 1\}$ with metric $ds^2 = 4\, |dz|^2 / (1 - |z|^2)^2$ (curvature $-1$):
- $\exp_x(v)$ via Möbius transformation: $\exp_x(v) = (x + \alpha) / (1 + \bar{x} \alpha)$ where $\alpha = \tanh(\|v\|_{g_x} / 2) \cdot v / \|v\|_{g_x}$ in the complex parameterisation. Closed-form, Anderson 2005 *Hyperbolic Geometry* §3.3.
- $P_{x \to y}(v)$: parallel transport along the geodesic from $x$ to $y$ — closed-form via the Möbius derivative.
- $R(x) \equiv -2$ (constant negative scalar curvature; sectional curvature $-1$ in 2D gives $R = 2 \cdot (-1)$).
- $\log \sqrt{\det g(x)} = \log(2 / (1 - |x|^2))$ — note the singularity as $|x| \to 1$; log-space arithmetic avoids underflow.

### §24.5 — Acceptance gates (G26 + T21N — NORMATIVE)

- **G26 slope gate** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0071): Sphere-$S^2$ heat-equation convergence. Initial datum: the first 4 spherical harmonics $Y_{\ell m}(\theta, \phi)$ for $(\ell, m) \in \{(0,0), (1,0), (1,1), (2,0)\}$ (truncated to a real-valued combination via $\cos(m\phi)$ component). Horizon $T = 0.05$ on $S^2$ discretized by an icosahedral mesh of $n^2$ cells ($n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ giving $\{256, 1024, 4096, 16384\}$ cells).

  Reference solution: $u(t, x) = \sum_{(\ell, m)} c_{\ell m} \exp(-\ell(\ell+1) t) Y_{\ell m}(x)$ (closed-form eigenfunction expansion; eigenvalues of $\Delta_{S^2}$ are $-\ell(\ell+1)$).

  **Sub-test 1** (base, NO curvature correction): construct `ManifoldChernoff<Sphere2<f64>>::new(sphere, false)`. Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|F^n(f_{\mathrm{init}}) - u(T, \cdot)\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST be $\le -0.95$ (order 1 per Theorem 24.1; -0.95 has 5% margin against the -1.0 asymptote). $n_{\mathrm{Chernoff}}$ iterations: $T / \tau$ with $\tau = 0.005$.

  **Sub-test 2** (with R/12 correction): construct `ManifoldChernoff<Sphere2<f64>>::new(sphere, true)`. Empirical slope MUST be $\le -1.95$ (order 2 per Theorem 24.1; -1.95 has 2.5% margin against the -2.0 asymptote).

  Both sub-tests use the SAME initial datum, SAME mesh sweep, SAME reference solution — the only difference is the `with_curvature_correction` flag. The order *promotion* from sub-test 1 to sub-test 2 is the key MMRS 2023 claim verified by G26.

  Test file: `tests/manifold_sphere_slope.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Both sub-tests MUST pass; failure BLOCKS v2.8 release.

- **T21N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0071): Flat-torus eigenmode exact identity. On $\mathbb{T}^2 = \mathbb{R}^2 / \mathbb{Z}^2$ with $R \equiv 0$, the Chernoff function (24.1) reduces to the standard heat kernel (the curvature correction vanishes identically). Verify symbolically that for the first 4 Fourier eigenmodes $\phi_{\mathbf{k}}(x, y) = \exp(2\pi i (k_x x + k_y y))$ with $\mathbf{k} \in \{(0,0), (1,0), (0,1), (1,1)\}$:
  $$
  F(\tau) \phi_{\mathbf{k}}(x, y) \;=\; \exp(-\tau \cdot 4\pi^2 |\mathbf{k}|^2) \cdot \phi_{\mathbf{k}}(x, y), \tag{T21N}
  $$
  EXACTLY (not approximately). The eigenvalues $-4\pi^2 |\mathbf{k}|^2$ are the standard Laplace-Beltrami eigenvalues on $\mathbb{T}^2$.

  Sympy sub-checks (mechanical):
  1. (T21N.curvature_zero) Verify symbolically that $R(x, y) = 0$ for the flat torus metric $g = \mathrm{diag}(1, 1)$ — uses `sympy.diffgeom` to compute the Ricci scalar from the Christoffel symbols; expected literally zero.
  2. (T21N.exp_map_identity) Verify $\exp_x(v) = x + v \pmod 1$ (modulo lattice) in normal coordinates — closed-form check.
  3. (T21N.eigenmode_action) Apply (24.1) symbolically to $\phi_{\mathbf{k}}$ with $R \equiv 0$ and $\exp_x(v) = x + v$; use `sympy.integrate` to evaluate the Gaussian integral over $T_x M = \mathbb{R}^2$ (the lattice quotient becomes a Riemann sum over $\mathbb{Z}^2$; for the first 4 eigenmodes the sum collapses to a single dominant term plus exponentially-small corrections, verified at machine precision by truncating after $|\mathbf{n}| \le 5$). Assert the result equals $\exp(-\tau \cdot 4\pi^2 |\mathbf{k}|^2) \cdot \phi_{\mathbf{k}}$.
  4. (T21N.spectral_consistency) Cross-check that the eigenvalue $4\pi^2 |\mathbf{k}|^2$ matches the standard Laplace-Beltrami spectrum on $\mathbb{T}^2$ — `sympy.simplify` reduction.

  Script: `scripts/verify_manifold_torus.py` (new file, ~120 LoC, ships with the v2.8 engineering wave). MUST print exactly `T21N PASS` on success or `T21N FAIL: <reason>` on failure. Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_resolvent_laplace_chernoff.py` and `verify_howland_lift.py`. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; safe for CI without `slow-tests`. Failure BLOCKS v2.8 release.

### §24.6 — `BoundedGeometryManifold<F>` trait + `ManifoldChernoff<M, F>` (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub trait BoundedGeometryManifold<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    /// Manifold dimension d.
    fn dim(&self) -> usize;

    /// Uniform infimum of injectivity radius: inj(M) := inf_{x ∈ M} inj(x).
    /// MUST be > 0 (bounded-geometry hypothesis B1).
    fn injectivity_radius(&self) -> F;

    /// Riemannian exponential map: out := exp_x(v).
    /// Writes d coordinates into `out`. Returns DomainViolation if
    /// `||v||_{g_x} >= inj(x)` (caller MUST stay within the injectivity ball).
    fn exp_map(&self, x: &[F], v: &[F], out: &mut [F]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;

    /// Parallel transport along the geodesic from x to y: out := P_{x→y}(v).
    /// Used by the Magnus-on-manifold higher-order extension (v3.x); shipped
    /// in v2.8 for completeness of the trait surface but not exercised by G26.
    fn parallel_transport(
        &self, x: &[F], y: &[F], v: &[F], out: &mut [F],
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;

    /// Scalar curvature R(x). MUST be uniformly bounded (hypothesis B2-B3).
    fn scalar_curvature(&self, x: &[F]) -> F;

    /// log √det g(x). Used by the volume-element change-of-variables in
    /// the Chernoff integrand. log-space for ULP stability near chart
    /// singularities (e.g., Poincaré disk boundary).
    fn volume_element_log(&self, x: &[F]) -> F;
}

pub struct ManifoldChernoff<M, F = f64>
where
    M: BoundedGeometryManifold<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    manifold: M,
    with_curvature_correction: bool,
    n_quad: usize,  // number of quadrature points on T_x M (default 32 per axis)
}

impl<M, F> ManifoldChernoff<M, F>
where
    M: BoundedGeometryManifold<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    pub fn new(manifold: M, with_curvature_correction: bool) -> Self;
}

impl<M, F> ChernoffFunction<F> for ManifoldChernoff<M, F>
where
    M: BoundedGeometryManifold<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    type S = ManifoldGridFn<F, M>;  // discretised function on M's mesh

    fn apply_into(
        &self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // For each grid cell x on M:
        //   evaluate the Gaussian-on-tangent integral (24.1) via
        //   tensor-product quadrature on T_x M with `n_quad` nodes per axis,
        //   using `manifold.exp_map(x, v_quad)` to pull back the integrand;
        //   apply the curvature correction [1 + (τ/12) R(x)] if enabled.
        //   write to dst[x].
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 {
        if self.with_curvature_correction { 2 } else { 1 }
    }

    fn growth(&self) -> (f64, f64) {
        (1.0, 0.0)  // heat semigroup on bounded-geometry manifold is contractive on the core
    }
}
```

### §24.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Three closed-form backends only.** User-defined manifolds COMPILE via the trait (the four geometric methods are filled in by the user) but are not gated by acceptance tests. Numerical geodesic flow (Runge-Kutta on the geodesic ODE) is deferred to v3.x once concrete use cases inform the API.
- **No higher-order correction.** Order-3 ($R^2$) and order-4 ($\nabla^2 R$) corrections are not shipped; require the full Riemann curvature tensor, not just the scalar — out of scope for v2.8.
- **Static metric only.** Time-dependent metric $g = g(t)$ (Ricci flow, mean curvature flow) is open math; `ManifoldChernoff` is explicitly NOT a `TimedChernoffFunction<F>` (ADR-0071 Rationale).
- **Real-valued only.** Complex-valued manifolds (Kähler structures, holomorphic line bundles) require complex-valued semigroup support — deferred to v4.0 B6 SemiflowComplex. **PARTIALLY RESOLVED at v7.0.0 (ADR-0129): the SCALAR Kähler heat backend on CP¹ (Fubini-Study) ships — see §24.7-bis. Holomorphic line-bundle SECTIONS remain deferred.**

### §24.7-bis — Scalar Kähler heat backend on CP¹ (v7.0.0, ADR-0129, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

The complex projective line $\mathbb{CP}^1$ with the **Fubini-Study metric** ships as an additive `BoundedGeometryManifold`-style backend over `SemiflowComplex`. The hinge fact (PRE-FLIGHT `scripts/verify_complex_kahler.py`, executed 2026-06-06, 3/3 PASS): $\mathbb{CP}^1$ with Fubini-Study is **isometric to the round $S^2$** — the affine-chart conformal factor $4/(1+|z|^2)^2$ is identical to $S^2$ stereographic projection, so the scalar Laplace-Beltrami operator (hence the heat semigroup on scalar functions) is the SAME real elliptic operator the shipped `Sphere2` backend evolves. Therefore the MMRS-2023 $[1+(\tau/12)R]$ curvature correction (§24.2) applies VERBATIM, with $R=2$ the (constant) Fubini-Study scalar curvature; NO new convergence theorem. The NEW content is solely the complex affine chart ($z\in\mathbb{C}$, complex-modulus `exp_map`/`scalar_curvature` over `SemiflowComplex`). PRE-FLIGHT verified: FS scalar curvature $R=2$ constant (curvature-kit Christoffel→Riemann→Ricci→scalar contraction); FS metric $\equiv$ $S^2$ stereographic; $[1+(\tau/12)R]$ tangent to $\exp(\tau R/12)$ to $O(\tau^2)$ (order preserved). Gate `G_KAHLER_CURV`: curvature-corrected self-convergence slope $\le -1.95$ (mirror G26 sphere). **Scope boundary (rustdoc MUST state):** this is the SCALAR Kähler heat backend (complex chart + FS metric); holomorphic line-bundle sections (genuinely complex-valued state, the $\bar\partial$-Laplacian on $\mathcal{O}(k)$) are a SEPARATE future deferral. References: MMRS 2023 *Math. Nachr.* Thm 1 (R/12); Kobayashi-Nomizu 1969 Vol II §IX.6 (Fubini-Study metric, $\mathbb{CP}^1\cong S^2(1/2)$ isometry).
- **No mesh adapter in `semiflow-core`.** The `ManifoldGridFn<F, M>` state type ASSUMES a flat array of per-cell values; the mesh structure (icosahedral for $S^2$, lattice for $\mathbb{T}^2$, hyperbolic tessellation for $\mathbb{H}^2$) lives in the backend impl. No `Mesh` trait in `semiflow-core` per ADR-0001 (no mesh primitives in core).

### §24.8 — References

- S. Mazzucchi, V. Moretti, I. Remizov, O. Smolyanov, *Operator semigroups and Chernoff approximations on Riemannian manifolds*, **Math. Nachr.** (2023). — Theorem 1 (the Gaussian-on-tangent-space Chernoff approximation with $R/12$ curvature correction); foundational citation for §24.2. The library reproduces only the formula (24.1); the proof of Theorem 24.1 lives in MMRS 2023 §4.
- J.-M. Bismut, *Large Deviations and Stochastic Mechanics*, Birkhäuser PM **45** (1984). — §3 (the Bismut-Driver formulation of the heat kernel on Riemannian manifolds via stochastic mechanics); cited for the geometric framework.
- T. Sakai, *Riemannian Geometry*, AMS Transl. Math. Monogr. **149** (1996). — §III.4 (Riemannian exponential map closed-form on $S^2$); reference for the Sphere2 backend.
- J. W. Anderson, *Hyperbolic Geometry*, Springer Undergrad. Math. Series (2nd ed., 2005). — §3.3 (Möbius transformation closed-form for exponential map on Poincaré disk); reference for the Hyperbolic2 backend.
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).
