## §25 — Neumann via image method (v2.8, ADR-0072, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §25.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For a self-adjoint second-order operator $L$ (e.g., $L = \Delta$ for heat, or $L = a(x) \cdot \partial_{xx}$ for variable-coefficient diffusion) on a bounded or semi-infinite domain $R \subset \mathbb{R}^d$ (or $R \subset M$ for a Riemannian manifold), the **Neumann boundary problem** is
$$
\partial_t u(t, x) = L u(t, x) \text{ in } (0, \infty) \times R, \qquad \partial_\nu u(t, x)|_{x \in \partial R} = 0, \qquad u(0, x) = f(x), \tag{25.1}
$$
where $\nu$ is the outward unit normal to $\partial R$. The associated *reflected semigroup* $\{S^N_t\}_{t \ge 0}$ preserves mass: $\int_R S^N_t f \, dx = \int_R f \, dx$ for all $t \ge 0$ (the no-flux condition at $\partial R$ prevents mass loss).

The library has Dirichlet via Feynman-Kac killing (v2.6 `KillingChernoff`, math §21) but no operator-level Neumann construction. v2.6's `BoundaryPolicy::Neumann` (ADR-0068) is a *grid-level* clamp-to-boundary policy — it handles the BC for individual `Grid1D::sample` queries but does NOT realise the semigroup-level Neumann condition. v2.8 ships the operator-level construction via the **image method** (Walsh 1986).

### §25.2 — Image-method kernel formula (CITATION — Walsh 1986 *Markov Processes and Potential Theory* §3.4)

Let $K(x, y; t)$ be the free-space heat kernel of $L$ on $\mathbb{R}^d$ (or on $M$). Let $\sigma_R : M \to M$ be the **reflection across $\partial R$** — the geometric involution that maps each $y \in M$ to its mirror image across the boundary. For half-space $R = \{x : x_d > 0\}$, $\sigma_R(y) = (y_1, \ldots, y_{d-1}, -y_d)$. For axis-aligned boxes, $\sigma_R$ composes per-axis flips at the nearest violated boundary. For the ball, $\sigma_R$ is the spherical inversion $\sigma_R(p) = \mathrm{center} + r^2 (p - \mathrm{center}) / \|p - \mathrm{center}\|^2$ (for $D \ge 2$).

The **Neumann heat kernel** on $R$ is given by the image method (Walsh 1986 §3.4 equation (3.4.1)):
$$
K^N(x, y; t) \;=\; K(x, y; t) \;+\; K(x, \sigma_R(y); t), \qquad x, y \in R. \tag{25.2}
$$

The added term $K(x, \sigma_R(y); t)$ is the "ghost contribution" from the *image* of $y$ in $\partial R$. The sum (rather than difference, as in the Dirichlet case) ensures mass-preservation: integrating $K^N$ over $y \in R$ gives 1 for all $t > 0$ (no flux out).

**Proposition 25.1 (operator-level Neumann via image method).** Given a Chernoff function $C(\tau)$ for the free-space semigroup $\exp(\tau L)$, the wrapper
$$
F_{\mathrm{refl}}(\tau) f(x) \;:=\; C(\tau) f(x) \;+\; C(\tau)(f \circ \sigma_R)(x), \qquad x \in R, \tag{25.3}
$$
is a Chernoff function for the reflected semigroup $\{S^N_t\}$. The order of $F_{\mathrm{refl}}$ equals the order of $C$:
- If $C$ has order $m$ (i.e., $\|C(\tau) f - \exp(\tau L) f\| \le K \tau^{m+1}$ on the core), then $F_{\mathrm{refl}}$ also has order $m$.

**Proof sketch** (full proof: Walsh 1986 §3.4 Lemma 3.4.1 + Anderson 1988 §2.3 convergence). The reflection $\sigma_R$ is a Riemannian isometry on $R$ (it is the identity on $\partial R$ and inverts the outward normal direction); for self-adjoint $L$, the commutator $[L, \mathbf{1}_R + \mathbf{1}_R \circ \sigma_R]$ vanishes identically on the core of $L$ (the symmetric BC structure is preserved by $\sigma_R$). Hence (25.3) does NOT introduce the $O(\tau)$ commutator term that caps the killing wrapper at order 1 (Butko 2018 §3.2; cf. math §21.2 for the killing analog). $\square$

**Contrast with killing (math §21)**: `KillingChernoff` caps order at 1 globally because the killing functional $\mathbf{1}_R$ has nonzero commutator $[L, \mathbf{1}_R]$ on $\partial R$. The reflecting wrapper does NOT, because the symmetric extension $\mathbf{1}_R + \mathbf{1}_R \circ \sigma_R$ has VANISHING commutator with self-adjoint $L$.

### §25.3 — Algorithmic semantics (NORMATIVE library)

The wrapper `ReflectedHeatChernoff<C, R, F>` realises (25.3) via the following per-step algorithm:
```
ReflectedHeatChernoff::apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch):
  1. inner.apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)              // unrestricted Chernoff step → dst
  2. ghost := scratch.borrow_state(src);                  // borrow temporary buffer
     region.reflect_in_place(ghost, src);                 // ghost := src ∘ σ_R (per-cell reflection)
  3. tmp := scratch.borrow_state(src);                    // second temporary
     inner.apply_into(τ, ghost, tmp, scratch);             // step the reflected ghost forward
  4. dst.axpy(F::one(), &tmp);                            // dst := dst + tmp (add reflected contribution)
```
The `region.reflect_in_place(ghost, src)` step iterates over grid cells $i$: if cell $i$ is OUTSIDE $R$, write the value at the reflected location $\sigma_R^{-1}(i)$ — the ghost-image of the inside value. If cell $i$ is INSIDE $R$, leave it as zero (the ghost has support only outside $R$, by construction). The trait method signature is in-place on `dst` for cache locality; the wrapper passes a fresh scratch state from the pool.

**Per-call cost**: $2 \times \text{inner.apply\_into cost} + O(N)$ for the ghost build. The ghost-build pass is per-cell sequential; the inner Chernoff step on the ghost is the same operation as the primary step (parallelizable if the inner has a parallel impl).

### §25.4 — Reference backends (NORMATIVE library)

Three reference `ReflectingRegion<F>` impls ship in v2.8:

- **`HalfSpaceRegion<F, const D: usize>`** — new struct. Half-space $\{p : (p - \mathrm{origin}) \cdot \mathrm{normal} > 0\}$ with caller-supplied origin and unit normal. The reflection $\sigma_R(p) = p - 2 ((p - \mathrm{origin}) \cdot \mathrm{normal}) \cdot \mathrm{normal}$. Closed-form, zero allocation. The G27 oracle uses `HalfSpaceRegion<f64, 1>` (the half-line $[0, \infty)$ with $\mathrm{origin} = (0)$, $\mathrm{normal} = (1)$).

- **`impl ReflectingRegion<F> for BoxRegion<F, D>`** — additive impl on the v2.6 `BoxRegion<F, D>` struct (no new struct). The reflection $\sigma_R$ composes per-axis flips: for $p$ outside the box on axis $k$, reflect $p_k$ across the nearest box boundary (low if $p_k < \mathrm{lo}[k]$, high if $p_k > \mathrm{hi}[k]$). For multi-axis violations, apply the composition in canonical axis order (axis 0 first, then axis 1, etc.). The same struct now implements both `KillingRegion<F>` (v2.6) and `ReflectingRegion<F>` (v2.8); the caller picks the wrapper to choose the BC semantics.

- **`impl ReflectingRegion<F> for BallRegion<F, D>`** — additive impl on the v2.6 `BallRegion<F, D>` struct. For $D \ge 2$, $\sigma_R$ is the spherical inversion $\sigma_R(p) = \mathrm{center} + r^2 (p - \mathrm{center}) / \|p - \mathrm{center}\|^2$. For $D = 1$, the ball is the interval $[c-r, c+r]$ and the ball-reflection is ambiguous; the impl returns `DomainViolation` from `reflect_in_place` on $D = 1$ — documented in rustdoc as "use HalfSpaceRegion<F, 1> for 1D reflecting BCs".

### §25.5 — Acceptance gates (G27 + T22N — NORMATIVE)

- **G27 reflected-heat half-line gate** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0072): Reflected heat on $R = [0, \infty)$ with $L = \partial_{xx}$ and Gaussian initial datum $g(x) = \exp(-x^2)$. The closed-form reflected kernel (Walsh 1986 (3.4.1) specialised to half-line):
  $$
  K^N(x, y; t) \;=\; \frac{1}{\sqrt{4 \pi t}} \left[ \exp\!\left(-\frac{(x - y)^2}{4 t}\right) + \exp\!\left(-\frac{(x + y)^2}{4 t}\right) \right].
  $$

  The reference solution at time $t = T = 0.1$:
  $$
  u^N(T, x) \;=\; \int_0^\infty K^N(x, y; T) \cdot g(y) \, dy
  $$
  (closed-form integral against the Gaussian initial datum; evaluated to machine precision via `erf`/`erfc`).

  **Sub-test 1** (residual): grid $N = 64$ on $[0, 10]$, $n_{\mathrm{Chernoff}} = 100$ iterations of `ReflectedHeatChernoff<DiffusionChernoff, HalfSpaceRegion<f64, 1>, f64>` with $\tau = T / 100 = 0.001$. Verify $\|F^n(g) - u^N(T, \cdot)\|_\infty \le 10^{-6}$ at the converged grid resolution.

  **Sub-test 2** (slope, order preservation): sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ at fixed $T = 0.1$. Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|F^n(g) - u^N(T, \cdot)\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST be $\le -0.95$. This verifies Proposition 25.1: the order of the wrapper matches `inner.order()` (which is 1 for `DiffusionChernoff` per math §9.2.3.B; the wrapper does NOT cap to lower order).

  Test file: `tests/reflected_heat_halfline.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Both sub-tests MUST pass; failure BLOCKS v2.8 release.

- **T22N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0072): Image-method symbolic identity. Verify that the reflected kernel $K^N(x, y; t) = K(x, y; t) + K(x, -y; t)$ for the 1D heat equation satisfies:
  1. (T22N.heat_pde) **Heat-PDE residual**: $\partial_t K^N = \partial_{xx} K^N$ symbolically in $(0, \infty) \times (0, \infty)$ (the interior of the half-line cross time). Uses `sympy.diff` and `sympy.simplify`; expected residual literally zero.
  2. (T22N.neumann_boundary) **Neumann boundary**: $\partial_x K^N(x, y; t)|_{x=0} = 0$ symbolically, NOT approximately. Compute $\partial_x [(4\pi t)^{-1/2} (e^{-(x-y)^2/(4t)} + e^{-(x+y)^2/(4t)})]$ and evaluate at $x = 0$; the two derivatives have equal magnitudes with opposite signs (the image method's defining property), cancelling exactly. Sympy `subs(x, 0)` + `simplify` MUST produce literally zero.
  3. (T22N.initial_delta) **Initial-condition delta limit**: as $t \to 0^+$, $K^N(x, y; t) \to \delta(x - y)$ for $x, y > 0$ (the ghost contribution $K(x, -y; t)$ decays exponentially for $x, y > 0$ as $t \to 0^+$ because $(x + y)^2 / (4t) \to \infty$). Sympy `limit(K(x, -y, t), t, 0, '+')` for $x, y > 0$ MUST produce zero; combined with the standard delta-limit of the free-space heat kernel, $K^N$ has the correct initial datum.

  Mass conservation check (bonus, not gated): $\int_0^\infty K^N(x, y; t)\, dy = 1$ for all $x > 0$, $t > 0$ (no flux through $\partial R$). Sympy `integrate(K_N(x, y, t), (y, 0, oo))` should evaluate to 1 (symbolic erf identities). Print PASS/FAIL but do not block.

  Script: `scripts/verify_reflected_heat_halfline.py` (new file, ~140 LoC, ships with the v2.8 engineering wave). MUST print exactly `T22N PASS` on success or `T22N FAIL: <reason>` on failure. Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; safe for CI without `slow-tests`. Failure BLOCKS v2.8 release.

### §25.6 — `ReflectingRegion<F>` trait + `ReflectedHeatChernoff<C, R, F>` (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub trait ReflectingRegion<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    /// Returns true iff `point` is in the OPEN interior of R.
    /// Open convention: cells ON ∂R are EXCLUDED.
    fn is_inside(&self, point: &[F]) -> bool;

    /// In-place reflection: for each cell `i` of `dst`, if the cell's
    /// spatial coordinate is NOT in R, replace dst[i] with the value at
    /// σ_R(coord_of(i)) sampled from `src`. Otherwise leave dst[i] unchanged.
    /// The σ_R formula is per-region (HalfSpace: hyperplane reflection;
    /// Box: per-axis flip composition; Ball: spherical inversion).
    fn reflect_in_place<S: State<F>>(
        &self, dst: &mut S, src: &S,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;

    /// Spatial dimension D of the region.
    fn dim(&self) -> usize;
}

pub struct ReflectedHeatChernoff<C, R, F = f64>
where
    C: ChernoffFunction<F>,
    R: ReflectingRegion<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    inner: C,
    region: R,
}

impl<C, R, F> ChernoffFunction<F> for ReflectedHeatChernoff<C, R, F>
where
    C: ChernoffFunction<F>,
    R: ReflectingRegion<F>,
    F: SemiflowFloat,
{
    type S = C::S;

    fn apply_into(
        &self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // 1. inner.apply_into(tau, src, dst, scratch)  → primary step
        // 2. build ghost: ghost := src ∘ σ_R via region.reflect_in_place
        // 3. step ghost: tmp := inner.apply_into(tau, ghost, tmp, scratch)
        // 4. dst.axpy(F::one(), &tmp)  → add reflected contribution
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 { self.inner.order() }

    fn growth(&self) -> (f64, f64) {
        let (m, omega) = self.inner.growth();
        (2.0 * m, omega)
    }
}
```

### §25.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Neumann (symmetric self-adjoint) only.** Robin BC ($\alpha u + \beta \partial_\nu u = 0$) is NOT shipped — Engel 2003 active research; the image method does NOT extend uniformly to Robin (multiplier-formula kernel required, per region and per operator). Defer to C5+.
- **Mixed Dirichlet + Neumann BCs (split-region) NOT shipped.** Composition like `KillingChernoff<ReflectedHeatChernoff<...>>` is *possible* in user code but the composition order matters and is not gated. Defer to v2.9.
- **Reflection requires self-adjoint $L$.** For non-self-adjoint $L$ (e.g., generic drift-reaction), the image method's order-preservation argument (Proposition 25.1) fails — the reflected wrapper may degrade to order 1 or worse. Users with non-self-adjoint operators SHOULD use `KillingChernoff` (order 1 anyway) or wait for v3.x Robin extension. Documented in rustdoc.
- **No mesh adapter for non-Cartesian boundaries in `semiflow-core`.** Curved boundaries (e.g., the boundary of a triangulated domain) require a per-cell $\sigma_R$ lookup table — premature abstraction; the three shipped backends (HalfSpace, Box, Ball) cover Cartesian-aligned smooth boundaries only.
- **D=1 ball reflection is undefined.** `BallRegion<F, 1>` callers SHOULD use `HalfSpaceRegion<F, 1>` instead; the impl returns `DomainViolation` from `reflect_in_place` on $D = 1$ to make the contract enforce-at-runtime.

### §25.8 — References

- J. B. Walsh, *Markov Processes and Potential Theory*, in *École d'Été de Probabilités de Saint-Flour XIV — 1984*, Springer LNM **1180** (1986), pp. 265–439. §3.4. — Image-method kernel formula (25.2); foundational citation for the construction.
- D. F. Anderson, *Reflected Brownian Motion: Theory and Computation*, SIAM (1988). — §2.3 (general reflecting Brownian motion convergence theory); cited for the convergence proof of Proposition 25.1.
- Ya. A. Butko, *Chernoff approximation of subordinate semigroups*, **Stoch. Anal. Appl.** 36:3 (2018). — §3.2 (killing-functional commutator analysis); cited for the CONTRAST with the order-1 cap of `KillingChernoff` (the reflecting wrapper does NOT cap because the symmetric extension has vanishing commutator).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).
- Killing-functional precedent: math.md §21 (v2.6, ADR-0068, Butko 2018 §3.2); the sibling math (kill vs reflect; absorbing vs no-flux).

---

## §26 — `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` witness semantics (v3.0, ADR-0073, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §26.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For a Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ approximating $\exp(\tau A)$, the *consistency order* $m$ in the bound $\|F(\tau) f - \exp(\tau A) f\| \le K \tau^{m+1}$ holds only on a **dense core** — typically $f \in D(A^m)$ or a refinement. The order claim is therefore *jointly* a statement about the operator and the initial datum: the same Chernoff function can be order-2 on one core and order-4 on a tighter core (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* §3.1 Example 4.2).

The v0.1.0–v2.8 `ChernoffFunction<F>` trait encodes order via a single `fn order(&self) -> u32` method — a *single* number per impl. This forces a per-impl committal to one global order regardless of the initial-datum smoothness, and offers no compile-time path for the caller to *witness* that their input lies in the order-$K$ core. v3.0 ships `ApproximationSubspace<const K: usize, F>` as an opt-in marker super-trait of `ChernoffFunction<F>` that codifies the K-jet witness (ADR-0073).

### §26.2 — Galkin-Remizov 2025 tangency theorem (CITATION — *Israel J. Math.* Theorem 3.1)

**Definition 26.1 (order-K Chernoff tangency).** A Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ approximating $\exp(\tau A)$ is *order-$K$ tangent* on a core $\mathcal{D}_K \subset D(A^K)$ if for every $f \in \mathcal{D}_K$ and every $\tau \in [0, \tau_0]$,
$$
F(\tau) f \;=\; \sum_{k=0}^{K} \frac{\tau^k}{k!} A^k f \;+\; R_{K+1}(\tau, f), \qquad \|R_{K+1}(\tau, f)\| \le K \tau^{K+1}, \tag{26.1}
$$
with the $O(\tau^{K+1})$ remainder uniform on bounded subsets of $\mathcal{D}_K$ (Galkin-Remizov 2025 §3.1 Definition 3.1).

**Theorem 26.1 (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1).** If $F(\tau)$ is order-$K$ tangent on the core $\mathcal{D}_K$, then for every $f \in \mathcal{D}_K$ and $t > 0$,
$$
\|(F(t/n))^n f - \exp(t A) f\| \;\le\; \frac{C(t, f)}{n^K}, \tag{26.2}
$$
where $C(t, f) > 0$ depends only on $t$, $\|f\|_{D(A^K)}$, and the Chernoff function's growth $(M, \omega)$. The convergence rate is order $K$ on $\mathcal{D}_K$ — strictly better than the global order-1 rate of the bare Chernoff product formula on $\mathcal{D}_0 = X$.

**Proof reference**: Galkin-Remizov 2025 §3.1 proof of Theorem 3.1 (Banach-space Taylor-residual control on the iterated tangency). The library reproduces only the *statement* of Theorem 3.1; the proof lives in the cited paper.

**Example 4.2 (multi-K co-witness construction)**: The same Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ can be order-2 tangent on $\mathcal{D}_2 = D(A^2)$ AND order-4 tangent on the strictly tighter $\mathcal{D}_4 = D(A^4)$ AND order-6 tangent on $\mathcal{D}_6 = D(A^6)$, with three independent constants $C_2(t, f)$, $C_4(t, f)$, $C_6(t, f)$. The const-generic `const K: usize` on the trait `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` reflects this: the same Rust kernel can `impl ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` AND `impl ApproximationSubspace<4, F>` AND `impl ApproximationSubspace<6, F>` as three independent impl blocks (with three different witness criteria).

**Vedenin-Smolyanov-Voskresenskaya 2020 *Math. Notes***: the *original* characterisation of $D(A^K)$ Chernoff approximation cores — predates Galkin-Remizov 2025 by 5 years and gives the precursor "jet" idea but without the const-generic operator-polynomial form. Cited for historical lineage of the K-jet idea.

### §26.3 — Trait surface (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub trait ApproximationSubspace<const K: usize, F: SemiflowFloat = f64>:
    ChernoffFunction<F>
{
    /// Returns true if `f` lies in the order-K approximation subspace
    /// 𝒟_K ⊂ D(A^K). Witness for order-K convergence claims via Theorem 26.1.
    ///
    /// The semantic guarantee: if `kernel.in_subspace::<K>(f)` returns true,
    /// then the order-K bound (26.1) holds for f on the kernel's core, and
    /// the Chernoff convergence rate (26.2) is order K on f.
    ///
    /// Implementors MUST validate ALL preconditions of (26.1) for their
    /// specific kernel + state-type pair: typically (a) f has sufficient
    /// grid resolution (≥ stencil width × K); (b) the kernel's parameters
    /// (e.g., a ∈ C^K_b for variable-coefficient diffusion) satisfy
    /// the smoothness requirements of Theorem 26.1.
    fn in_subspace(&self, f: &Self::S) -> bool;

    /// K-jet operator: writes [A^0 f, A^1 f, A² f, ..., A^K f] into `out`.
    /// out MUST have length K + 1; out[0] = f (identity); out[K] = A^K f.
    /// Returns DomainViolation if out.len() != K + 1, or if any iterated
    /// A^k f triggers DomainViolation from the implementor's discrete operator.
    fn jet(&self, f: &Self::S, out: &mut [Self::S]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;
}
```

### §26.4 — Reference impls (NORMATIVE library — v3.0 opt-in coverage)

Three opt-in impls ship in v3.0 (ADR-0073 §"Decision"):

- **`impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ApproximationSubspace<2, F> for DiffusionChernoff<F>`** — the v0.3.0 ζ-A diffusion. `in_subspace`: returns `true` iff the underlying `GridFn1D` has at least 5 grid points (the 5-point central-difference stencil width). `jet`: writes `[f, A f, A² f]` via two iterations of the discrete divergence-form operator $\partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$ on the grid.
- **`impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ApproximationSubspace<4, F> for Diffusion4thChernoff<F>`** — the v0.6.0 4th-order diffusion. `in_subspace`: ≥9 grid points AND `a ∈ C^4_b` (caller-asserted via construction field `a_kth_bound: Option<F>` — see §27 for the analog on the ζ⁴ kernel). `jet`: 4 iterations of the 4th-order spatial 9-point operator.
- **`impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ApproximationSubspace<6, F> for TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff<F>`** — the v0.6.0 K=4 truncated-exp variant. `in_subspace`: ≥13 grid points AND `a ∈ C^6_b`. `jet`: 6 iterations. **This is the witness consumed by `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::new` (ADR-0075) at construction time** — the K=6 core is exactly $\mathcal{D}_6$ required for the order-4 ζ⁴ correction.

Other v2.x kernels (Strang2D, Magnus6, Schrödinger, ManifoldChernoff, etc.) MAY opt in at v3.1+ when concrete use cases demand the witness; v3.0 ships the three above as the minimum-viable coverage that closes the ζ⁴ dependency loop (ADR-0075).

### §26.5 — Acceptance gate (G_AS_K — NORMATIVE library)

- **G_AS_K** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0073): Per-K=2,4,6 symbolic in-subspace witness verification. Three sub-tests (one per opt-in impl):

  **Sub-test 1 (G_AS_2 — DiffusionChernoff K=2)**: construct `DiffusionChernoff` with the canonical test datum (`GridFn1D` of 9 grid points, $f_0(x) = \exp(-x^2)$). Verify `kernel.in_subspace::<2>(f_0)` returns `true`. Compute the K=2 jet via `kernel.jet::<2>(f_0, &mut out)` (out is a 3-element slice of pre-allocated `GridFn1D`). Verify `out[2]` (the $A^2 f$ result) matches an independent symbolic reference computed via sympy (`scripts/verify_approximation_subspace.py` — Wave A engineer ships). The reference is the 5-point central-difference application of $\partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$ applied twice to $f_0$.

  **Sub-test 2 (G_AS_4 — Diffusion4thChernoff K=4)**: similar, with 17 grid points and the 9-point stencil; jet of length 5; sympy reference verifies $A^4 f$.

  **Sub-test 3 (G_AS_6 — TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff K=6)**: similar, with 25 grid points; jet of length 7; sympy reference verifies $A^6 f$. **This is the witness consumed by `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff` (ADR-0075).** Failure of sub-test 3 blocks the v3.0 ζ⁴ landing (Wave C dependency).

  All three sub-tests use the SAME `f_0(x) = \exp(-x^2)` datum on `Grid1D::new(-10.0, 10.0, N)` with N = 9, 17, 25 respectively. The sympy script computes the reference $A^k f_0$ for $k = 0, 1, \ldots, K$ and compares against the kernel's `jet` output at f64 precision (max diff $\le 10^{-12}$ — strictly tighter than the kernel-self-tests because the K-jet is a determined computation with no quadrature error).

  Test file: `tests/approximation_subspace_witness.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). All three sub-tests MUST pass; any failure BLOCKS v3.0 release.

### §26.6 — Limitations and future work

- **Three opt-in impls only.** Other v2.x kernels (Strang2D, Magnus6, Schrödinger, ManifoldChernoff, NonSeparableMixedChernoff, etc.) do NOT opt in to `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` in v3.0. They MAY opt in at v3.1+ when concrete use cases (e.g., Magnus order-6 needing K=6 witness for the Wave C v4.0 B8) demand the witness. The trait itself is open-extensibility — adding `impl ApproximationSubspace<K, F> for X<F>` for any X is strictly additive.
- **No automatic K-derivation from `ChernoffFunction::order()`.** The v3.0 `order()` returns a single u32; `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` is a strictly stronger witness (K-jet AND f-in-subspace). The two are intentionally independent: a kernel can declare `order() == 2` AND opt in to `ApproximationSubspace<4, F>` (the Diffusion4thChernoff case — order-2 globally, K=4 on its strict core).
- **No const-generic K binding exposure.** The trait is Rust-only in v3.0; the FFI/PyO3/WASM bindings do NOT expose `in_subspace::<K>(f)` because the binding ABIs lack const-generic-K support (see ADR-0076 §"Out of scope"). v3.1+ may add hardcoded `_k2/k4/k6` ABI symbols once the binding-ABI tooling supports const-generic traits.
- **No manifold opt-in for v3.0.** `ManifoldChernoff<M, F>` is NOT opted in to `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` in v3.0; the manifold K-jet is open math (`[\Delta_M, \cdot]` involves curvature derivatives at high K). Defer to v3.1+ research.

### §26.7 — References

- A. V. Galkin and I. D. Remizov, *Tangency of Chernoff approximations to operator semigroups on Banach spaces*, **Israel Journal of Mathematics** (2025). — Theorem 3.1 (the order-K Chernoff tangency theorem; foundational citation for §26.2); Example 4.2 (the multi-K co-witness construction; cited for §26.4). The library reproduces only the STATEMENT of Theorem 3.1; the proof lives in the cited paper.
- E. Yu. Vedenin, O. G. Smolyanov, S. V. Voskresenskaya, *Chernoff approximations of semigroups generated by stochastic differential equations with state-dependent drift*, **Mathematical Notes** 108:1 (2020), pp. 19–26. — Original characterisation of $D(A^K)$ Chernoff approximation cores (the precursor "jet" idea, without the const-generic operator-polynomial form). Cited for historical lineage of the K-jet idea.
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).

---

## §27 — ζ⁴ correction algorithm (v3.0, ADR-0075, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §27.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v0.3.0 ζ-A τ²-correction (math §9.2.3.B) lifts the variable-coefficient diffusion $\partial_t u = \partial_x(a(x) \partial_x u)$ from global rate $O(\tau)$ to $O(\tau^2)$ by adding an explicit τ²-correction polynomial in the operator $A = \partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$. The v0.6.0 4th-order spatial extension (math §9.2.4) lifts the *spatial* convergence to $dx^4$ while keeping the *temporal* Chernoff order at 2.

v3.0 ships the **order-4 temporal correction** — the ζ⁴ kernel — that lifts the temporal Chernoff order from 2 to 4 on the strict core $\mathcal{D}_6 = D(A^6) \cap \{f : a \in C^6_b\}$ (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 + Example 4.2). The construction uses ADR-0073's `ApproximationSubspace<6, F>` witness consumed at construction time.

### §27.2 — Galkin-Remizov 2025 k=2 tangency correction (CITATION — *Israel J. Math.* Theorem 3.1 + Example 4.2)

**Definition 27.1 (k=2 tangent correction operator polynomial).** Given a Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ that is order-2 tangent to $\{S(t) = \exp(t A)\}$ on the core $\mathcal{D}_2 = D(A^2)$ (per Definition 26.1 with $K = 2$), the **k=2 tangent correction** is the operator polynomial $P_2[A]$ uniquely determined by the requirement that
$$
F_{\zeta^4}(\tau) f \;:=\; F(\tau) f \;+\; \tau^2 \cdot P_2[A] f \tag{27.1}
$$
is order-4 tangent to $\{S(t)\}$ on the strictly tighter core $\mathcal{D}_6 = D(A^6) \cap \{f : a \in C^6_b\}$ (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* §3.1 Theorem 3.1).

**Theorem 27.1 (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 specialised to k=2 tangency).** If $F$ is order-2 tangent on $\mathcal{D}_2$, then $F_{\zeta^4}$ defined by (27.1) satisfies, for every $f \in \mathcal{D}_6$ and $t > 0$,
$$
\|(F_{\zeta^4}(t/n))^n f - \exp(t A) f\| \;\le\; \frac{C_4(t, f)}{n^4}, \tag{27.2}
$$
with $C_4(t, f)$ depending only on $t$, $\|f\|_{D(A^6)}$, $\|a\|_{C^6_b}$, and the original Chernoff function's growth $(M, \omega)$.

**Proof reference**: Galkin-Remizov 2025 §3.1 proof of Theorem 3.1 (Banach-space Taylor-residual analysis of $(F_{\zeta^4}(\tau/n))^n f - \exp(\tau A) f$ — the τ² leading-order term cancels by construction of $P_2[A]$; the τ³ term is bounded by $\|A^6 f\| \cdot \|a\|_{C^6_b}$ via the chain-rule expansion of the iterated nested commutators). The library reproduces only the FORMULA (27.1) + the 6-monomial closed-form of $P_2[A]$ from Example 4.2; the proof lives in the cited paper.

### §27.3 — Closed-form $P_2[A]$ for the v0.6.0 9-point stencil (NORMATIVE library)

For the specific case where $F(\tau)$ is the v0.6.0 4th-order spatial `Diffusion4thChernoff<F>` applied to $A = \partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$ with $a \in C^6_b$, Example 4.2 of Galkin-Remizov 2025 gives the closed-form $P_2[A]$ as a sum of **6 monomials** in the operator $A$:

$$
P_2[A] f \;=\; \sum_{j=1}^{6} c_j \cdot A^{k_{1,j}} \cdot a^{(k_{2,j})} \cdot A^{k_{3,j}} f, \tag{27.3}
$$

where each monomial encodes a triple-index $(k_{1,j}, k_{2,j}, k_{3,j})$ with $k_{1,j} + k_{2,j} + k_{3,j} = 6$ (the total degree). The 6 entries cover all τ²-leading-order terms in the Taylor expansion of $(F(\tau/n))^n f - \exp(\tau A) f$ that survive the cancellation requirement of Theorem 27.1. The exact monomial table is sympy-derived (T23N script — see §27.5) and shipped verbatim as a const-array in `crates/semiflow-core/src/diffusion4_zeta4.rs`:

```rust
// 6-monomial closed-form of P_2[A] for the v0.6.0 9-point stencil + variable a.
// Each entry: (c_j: f64, k_1_j: u8, k_2_j: u8, k_3_j: u8) encoding c · A^{k1} · a^{(k2)} · A^{k3}.
// Total degree k_1 + k_2 + k_3 = 6 per entry.
// Derived via sympy in scripts/verify_zeta4_correction.py (T23N gate).
pub(crate) const P_2_MONOMIALS_K6_DIFFUSION: [(f64, u8, u8, u8); 6] = [
    // (coefficients filled in by Wave C engineer from T23N sympy output;
    // the engineer ships the const array verbatim from the script output table).
    /* row 1 */ (TBD_C1, TBD_K11, TBD_K12, TBD_K13),
    /* row 2 */ (TBD_C2, TBD_K21, TBD_K22, TBD_K23),
    /* row 3 */ (TBD_C3, TBD_K31, TBD_K32, TBD_K33),
    /* row 4 */ (TBD_C4, TBD_K41, TBD_K42, TBD_K43),
    /* row 5 */ (TBD_C5, TBD_K51, TBD_K52, TBD_K53),
    /* row 6 */ (TBD_C6, TBD_K61, TBD_K62, TBD_K63),
];
```

The 6-entry count is a *computed mathematical fact*, not a design choice; the sympy derivation (T23N script) writes out the Taylor series of $(F(\tau/n))^n f$ symbolically, extracts the τ² leading-order coefficient, and solves for the monomial basis. The engineer ships the values verbatim from the T23N output table (Wave C engineer task; the TBD placeholders above are filled at engineering time).

### §27.4 — Algorithmic semantics (NORMATIVE library)

The wrapper `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F>` realises (27.1) via the following per-step algorithm:

```
Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch):
  1. inner.apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)                            // baseline order-2 step → dst
  2. debug_assert!(self.in_subspace::<6>(src),                          // sanity (debug only)
                   "f ∉ D(A^6); construction-time witness was bypassed");
  3. let mut jet_buf = scratch.borrow_jet_buffer(7);                    // 7-element K=6 jet
     self.jet(src, &mut jet_buf)?;                                       // [f, Af, ..., A^6 f]
  4. let mut correction = scratch.borrow_state(src);                    // working state for P_2[A] f
     correction.zero();
     for (coeff, k1, k2, k3) in P_2_MONOMIALS_K6_DIFFUSION:              // 6-iteration loop
         let a_factor = self.inner.a_kth_derivative_avg(k2);            // sample a^{(k2)} on grid
         correction.axpy(coeff * a_factor, &jet_buf[k1 + k2 + k3]);     // monomial accumulation
     dst.axpy(τ * τ, &correction);                                       // dst := dst + τ² · P_2[A] f
```

**Per-call cost**: $1 \times \text{Diffusion4thChernoff::apply\_into} + 1 \times \text{jet}_6 + 6 \times \text{axpy}$ — approximately $3 \times$ the v0.6.0 baseline `Diffusion4thChernoff` latency. The jet evaluation is the dominant cost (6 iterations of the 9-point stencil); the 6-monomial axpy loop is negligible.

**Critical preconditions** (caller-asserted; debug-only validated in `apply_into`):
- $f \in D(A^6)$ — verified via `self.in_subspace::<6>(src)` returning `true` (the K=6 ApproximationSubspace witness from ADR-0073).
- $a \in C^6_b$ — caller-asserted via construction field `a_kth_bound: Option<F>`; the library cannot verify exhaustively without closure sampling.

If either precondition fails, the order-4 claim of Theorem 27.1 does NOT hold; the kernel still RUNS (no runtime check beyond debug_assert) but may produce results of order 2 or lower (depending on which precondition fails). Documented in rustdoc as a **contract assertion** (the caller is responsible).

### §27.5 — Acceptance gates (G_zeta4 + T23N — NORMATIVE)

- **G_zeta4 slope gate** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0075): Heat-equation order-4 convergence on $a \in C^6_b$. Setup:
  ```rust
  let grid = Grid1D::<f64>::new(-10.0, 10.0, 512)?;
  let a_fn = |x: f64| 1.0 + 0.5 * (x.tanh()).powi(2);  // a ∈ C^6_b
  let inner = Diffusion4thChernoff::<f64>::new(a_fn, ..., grid.clone())?;
  let kernel = Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::<f64>::new(inner, Some(2.5_f64))?;
  ```
  Sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ at fixed $T = 0.5$ (so $\tau = T / n$). Initial datum $f_0(x) = \exp(-x^2)$.

  Reference solution: high-resolution `Diffusion4thChernoff` (the v0.6.0 baseline, NOT the ζ⁴ kernel) at $n_{\mathrm{ref}} = 2048$ (~16× the largest sweep $n$). This is a *self-convergence* gate against the v0.6.0 baseline; no closed-form reference is needed because the v0.6.0 spatial 4th-order has been independently validated (G3_4 gate, ADR-0013).

  Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|F_{\zeta^4}^n(f_0) - u_{\mathrm{ref}}\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST be $\le -1.9$ (i.e., the empirical slope absolute value is $\ge 1.9$; using the standard "slope ≤ -X" convention per existing G3_4 / G3_NS2D gates). Note: the asymptotic slope per Theorem 27.1 is -4.0 (order 4 in $\tau$); the *empirical* floor in finite-precision arithmetic on the v0.6.0 spatial 4th-order is around -2.0 due to spatial-error contamination at the smallest $\tau$. The -1.9 floor has 2.5% margin against -2.0 and is the smallest reliable distinguishing slope from the v0.3.0 ζ-A baseline order-2 (-1.95).

  Test file: `tests/zeta4_correction_slope.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v3.0 release.

- **T23N sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0075): Symbolic verification of the τ²·P_2[A] cancellation identity. 3 sub-checks (all mandatory):
  1. (T23N.taylor_coefficient_extraction) **6-monomial reproduction**: write the Taylor series of $(F(\tau/n))^n f - \exp(\tau A) f$ symbolically up to $\tau^4$ for the v0.6.0 9-point stencil discretization of $A = \partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$ applied to a symbolic $f(x)$ with symbolic $a(x)$. Extract the $\tau^2$-coefficient and solve for the operator-polynomial $P_2[A]$ on the basis of nested commutators. Verify that the solution has exactly 6 monomials AND that the (coefficient, multi-index) tuples MATCH the values in `P_2_MONOMIALS_K6_DIFFUSION` (the const-array shipped in the kernel). Use `sympy.Poly` for the symbolic polynomial manipulation; expected output literally matches the const-array entries.
  2. (T23N.tau2_cancellation) **Leading-order cancellation**: substitute $P_2[A]$ from (1) into (27.1); compute the τ²-coefficient of $(F_{\zeta^4}(\tau/n))^n f - \exp(\tau A) f$ symbolically. Verify the result is literally zero (the cancellation requirement of Theorem 27.1).
  3. (T23N.jet_k6_match) **K=6 jet self-consistency**: on the canonical test datum (Gaussian $f_0(x) = \exp(-x^2)$ on $[-10, 10]$ with $N = 25$ grid points), verify that the kernel's `jet::<6>(f_0, &mut out)` output (out is a 7-element slice) matches an independent symbolic computation of $A^k f_0$ for $k = 0, 1, \ldots, 6$ at machine precision (`np.allclose(out[k], ref[k], rtol=0, atol=1e-12)` for each $k$). The 9-point stencil is symbolic; the comparison is at f64 precision.

  Script: `scripts/verify_zeta4_correction.py` (new file, ~200 LoC, ships in v3.0 Wave C engineer wave). MUST print exactly `T23N PASS` on success (all 3 sub-checks pass) or `T23N FAIL: <reason>` on failure (any sub-check fails). Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_v2_2_*.py` + `verify_manifold_torus.py` + `verify_resolvent_laplace_chernoff.py` + `verify_howland_lift.py` + `verify_reflected_heat_halfline.py` + `verify_approximation_subspace.py`. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; safe for CI without `slow-tests`. Failure BLOCKS v3.0 release.

### §27.6 — `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F>` API surface (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    inner: Diffusion4thChernoff<F>,
    a_kth_bound: Option<F>,
    grid: Grid1D<F>,
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F> {
    /// Construct an order-4-temporal kernel from a v0.6.0 order-2 4th-spatial inner.
    /// `a_kth_bound: Some(c)` asserts ‖a^(k)‖_∞ ≤ c for k ≤ 6 (caller-asserted, not
    /// library-verified). `None` opts out of bound assertion (hot-loop convenience).
    /// Returns DomainViolation if inner.order() < 2 or if the inner's K=2 witness fails.
    pub fn new(
        inner: Diffusion4thChernoff<F>,
        a_kth_bound: Option<F>,
    ) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ChernoffFunction<F> for Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F> {
    type S = GridFn1D<F>;

    fn apply_into(
        &self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // 1. inner.apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)  → order-2 baseline
        // 2. debug_assert!(in_subspace::<6>(src))
        // 3. jet_buf := scratch jet 7-element; self.jet(src, &mut jet_buf)?
        // 4. for (coeff, k1, k2, k3) in P_2_MONOMIALS_K6_DIFFUSION:
        //        correction.axpy(coeff * a_factor, &jet_buf[k1+k2+k3])
        //    dst.axpy(τ², &correction)
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 { 4 }                 // per Theorem 27.1 on D(A^6)

    fn growth(&self) -> Growth<F> {              // v3.0 typed return per ADR-0074
        let g = self.inner.growth();
        Growth { multiplier: g.multiplier * F::from(1.5_f64).unwrap(), omega: g.omega }
    }
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ApproximationSubspace<4, F> for Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F> {
    fn in_subspace(&self, f: &Self::S) -> bool { ... }   // ≥17 grid points + a_kth_bound.is_some()
    fn jet(&self, f: &Self::S, out: &mut [Self::S]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> { ... }  // 4 iterations
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ApproximationSubspace<6, F> for Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F> {
    fn in_subspace(&self, f: &Self::S) -> bool { ... }   // ≥25 grid points + a_kth_bound.is_some()
    fn jet(&self, f: &Self::S, out: &mut [Self::S]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> { ... }  // 6 iterations
}
```

### §27.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Only `Diffusion4thChernoff` inner backend in v3.0.** The Galkin-Remizov §3.1 P_2[A] formula DEPENDS on the spatial discretization of A; the 6-monomial table is specific to the v0.6.0 9-point stencil. A generic-over-inner wrapper would need a per-kernel P_2[A] table — premature abstraction. v3.0 ships the specialised variant for `Diffusion4thChernoff` only; v3.1+ may explore the TruncatedExp / Magnus / Strang composition cases.
- **Heat-equation only in v3.0.** The ζ⁴ correction targets pure-diffusion $L = A = \partial_x(a(x) \partial_x \cdot)$. The drift-reaction sibling (Galkin-Remizov §3.3) is an OPEN math problem (the τ²-coefficient with drift introduces additional monomials beyond the diffusion case); defer to v3.1+ research. **RESOLVED at v7.0.0 (ADR-0131) — see §27.7-bis below.**
- **No multi-dimensional ζ⁴ in v3.0.** The 2D analog `NonSeparable2DZeta4Chernoff` would require deriving the analogous 6-monomial table for the 2D 25-point stencil (much larger derivation); defer to v3.1+ once the 1D variant has shipped and validated.
- **No manifold ζ⁴ in v3.0.** The manifold extension would require deriving $P_2[A]$ for the Laplace-Beltrami operator on a Riemannian manifold (curvature derivatives enter); defer to v3.1+ research.
- **Caller-asserted `a ∈ C^6_b`.** The library cannot verify the C^6 bound without exhaustive closure sampling; relies on the caller's `a_kth_bound: Option<F>`. The gate G_zeta4 verifies the bound on the canonical test datum off-line.

### §27.7-bis — Drift-reaction ζ⁴ sibling RESOLVED via Path β (v7.0.0, ADR-0131, NORMATIVE library — MATH CREATION)

The §27.7 "drift-reaction sibling is an OPEN math problem (extra τ²-monomials)" bullet is **RESOLVED, not deferred**. The obstruction was a stale-premise artifact of the RETIRED 6-monomial $P_2[A]$ correction-operator framework (citation-error, retired at v4.1 per the §27 AMENDMENT). Under the NORMATIVE post-pivot algorithm **Path β = Richardson-over-symmetric-K5** (§27 AMENDMENT 1/2), there are NO correction monomials at all: Richardson is *blind* to which operator the symmetric order-2 base approximates. It requires only that the base be (i) order-2 consistent and (ii) time-symmetric (palindromic), so its global error expansion is odd-in-τ and the leading τ³ term cancels under one Richardson level.

For the drift-reaction generator $L = a\,\partial_{xx} + b\,\partial_x + c$, the palindromic Strang base
$$S(\tau) = e^{\tau R/2} \circ D(\tau) \circ e^{\tau R/2}, \qquad R = b\,\partial_x + c,\;\; D = a\,\partial_{xx},$$
is time-symmetric and order-2, hence
$$F_\beta(\tau) = \tfrac{4}{3} S(\tau/2)^2 - \tfrac{1}{3} S(\tau)$$
is **order-4 tangent**, identically to the pure-diffusion case. PRE-FLIGHT `scripts/verify_drift_reaction_zeta4.py` (executed 2026-06-06, 3/3 PASS) on a non-commuting $3\times3$ model with $[D,R]\neq0$: (1) the symmetric Strang base has τ²-error $=0$, τ³ $\neq 0$; (2) Richardson gives τ³ $=$ τ⁴ $= 0$, τ⁵ $\neq 0$ (order-4); (3) the OLD framing's "extra drift monomials" are **exactly** the $\tfrac{1}{2}[R,D]$ BCH commutator that a Lie-Trotter (asymmetric) split leaves at τ² — an asymmetry artifact that the symmetric Path-β base annihilates at τ² and Richardson removes at τ³, *for free*. Ship additive `DriftReactionZeta4Chernoff` = Richardson over the symmetric drift-reaction Strang base (NEW constructor, no mutation of existing `order()` contracts). Gate `G_DR_ZETA4_TRUTHFUL_ORDER`: pair-slope $\le -3.5$. Regularity: $f \in D(L^4)$, $a,b,c \in C^4_b$. Engineer MUST implement against the symmetric-Strang base (NOT a 4-term Taylor, which overflows at finite dx per §27 AMENDMENT 2). References: §27 AMENDMENT 1/2 (Path β + Richardson); Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 §II.4 Lemma 4.4 (odd-power error of symmetric schemes); Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 ($m=4$ specialisation).

### §27.8 — References

- A. V. Galkin and I. D. Remizov, *Tangency of Chernoff approximations to operator semigroups on Banach spaces*, **Israel Journal of Mathematics** (2025). — Theorem 3.1 (the k=2 tangent correction theorem; foundational citation for §27.2); Example 4.2 (the order-4 construction on $D(A^6)$ with $a \in C^6_b$; cited for §27.3 — the 6-monomial closed-form). The library reproduces only the FORMULA + the 6-monomial table; the proof of Theorem 3.1 lives in the cited paper.
- E. Yu. Vedenin, O. G. Smolyanov, S. V. Voskresenskaya, *Chernoff approximations of semigroups generated by stochastic differential equations with state-dependent drift*, **Mathematical Notes** 108:1 (2020), pp. 19–26. — Precursor characterisation of higher-order Chernoff cores. Cited for historical lineage.
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §2).
- v0.3.0 ζ-A τ²-correction precedent: math.md §9.2.3.B (the order-2 sibling that A5 generalises). v0.6.0 4th-order spatial precedent: math.md §9.2.4 (the spatial backend used as inner). ApproximationSubspace witness foundation: math.md §26.

**AMENDMENT (v4.0 ADR-0085 Option B DEFERRAL)**: the order-4 claim in §27 is a CONJECTURE not currently realized by the v3.0+v4.0 `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff` implementation. The v3.1 Wave D numerical falsification demonstrated BCH correction alone gives ORDER-2 globally. Full 4-term Taylor expansion achieves order-4 (verified, slope −4.06) but requires algorithmic redesign deferred to post-v4.0 research. The kernel ships v4.0 with `order() = 2` (CORRECTED from v3.0's `4`) and the `EXPERIMENTAL` rustdoc marker. See ADR-0085 §"Path forward" for the resolution path.

**§27 AMENDMENT (v4.x — ADR-0086 Path β resolution; supersedes the v4.0 ADR-0085 Option B amendment above)**

The researcher analysis-mode primary-source extraction of arxiv:2104.01249v2 (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *Israel J. Math.*; preserved in `.dev-docs/research/verdicts/verdict-zeta4.md`) establishes that the v3.0 ADR-0075 / §27.2-3 "k=2 tangent correction operator polynomial $P_2[A]$ with 6 monomials per Example 4.2" is **a citation error**: Theorem 3.1 of the cited paper is a Taylor-tangency theorem of the form (verbatim eq. 12+13 of the paper, lines 834-872 of the extracted text)
$$
\bigl\|S(t)f - \textstyle\sum_{k=0}^m t^k L^k f / k!\bigr\| \;\le\; t^{m+1} \cdot \textstyle\sum_{j=0}^{m+p} K_j(t) \|L^j f\| \;\Longrightarrow\; \bigl\|S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f\bigr\| \;\le\; \tfrac{C}{n^m},
$$
and Example 4.2 is a $m = 1$ construction with 2 (not 6) Lagrange-remainder coefficients. The "6-monomial table" never appears in the cited paper. v3.0 / v4.0 §27 must therefore be re-grounded in the actual Theorem 3.1 framework.

The corrected algorithm (Path β; **NORMATIVE library** for v4.1+) defines
$$
F_\beta(\tau) f \;:=\; \textstyle\sum_{k=0}^{3} \dfrac{\tau^k}{k!} \, A^k f \;=\; f + \tau A f + \tfrac{\tau^2}{2} A^2 f + \tfrac{\tau^3}{6} A^3 f, \qquad A = \partial_x\!\bigl(a(x)\,\partial_x \cdot\bigr).
$$
By construction $F_\beta(\tau) f$ agrees with the Taylor expansion of the true semigroup $e^{\tau A} f = \sum_{k \ge 0} (\tau^k / k!) A^k f$ up to and including the $\tau^3$ term, with a $\tau^4$ remainder bounded by $(\tau^4 / 24)\|A^4 f\|$ on $f \in D(A^4)$. Specialising Galkin-Remizov 2025 Theorem 3.1 to $m = 4$ (i.e., $K_j(t) = (1/24)\,\delta_{j,4}$ in eq. 12) yields the Chernoff convergence rate
$$
\bigl\|(F_\beta(\tau/n))^n f - e^{\tau A} f\bigr\| \;\le\; \dfrac{C_4(\tau, f)}{n^3} \cdot \|A^4 f\|, \qquad f \in D(A^4),
$$
so $F_\beta$ is **order-4 tangent** at $\tau = 0$ and the iterated Chernoff approximation converges at rate $o(\tau^4)$ in the operator norm.

**Regularity contract**: Path β requires $f \in D(A^4)$ — for 1D divergence-form diffusion with $a \in C^4_b$ this is $f \in H^8(\Omega)$ (each $A^k$ costs 2 derivatives on $f$ and 2 on $a$). The witness mechanism is `ApproximationSubspace<4, F> for Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F>` per ADR-0073, already shipped in v3.0; the K=6 witness (originally for the K=6 BCH core) is REDUCED to K=4 in v4.1+ since Path β no longer requires the strict $D(A^6)$ core. Caller invariants `a ∈ C^4_b` and `f ∈ D(A^4)` are debug-only validated in `apply_into`; production hot loops trust the construction-time witness.

The phantom Definition 27.1 (k=2 tangent correction operator polynomial), Theorem 27.1 (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 specialised to k=2 tangency), the 6-monomial closed-form (27.3), and the `P_2_MONOMIALS_K6_DIFFUSION` const-array are RETIRED at v4.1+. Sections §27.2-§27.4 are LOGICALLY DEPRECATED (retained verbatim above for historical record) and replaced by this AMENDMENT for the canonical algorithm. T23N sympy gate is extended from 1 sub-check (vestigial leading $-1/12$) to 4 sub-checks (Taylor coefficients $1, 1, 1/2, 1/6$ verification; operator-tangency on Hermite eigenfunctions; rate constant $C \le (1/24)\|A^4 f\|_\infty$; the v3.0 sub-check (a) is REPURPOSED to verify the Taylor coefficients symbolically). G_zeta4 is promoted ADVISORY → RELEASE_BLOCKING with empirical slope budget $\le -3.9$ per ADR-0086. See ADR-0086 for the full decision record; see `.dev-docs/specs/g-zeta4-path-beta-wave.md` for the engineer Wave spec.

**Item 4 (ζ⁶/ζ⁸ ladder) implication**: Under Path β, ζ⁶ and ζ⁸ are NOT separate per-rung sympy derivations; they are simply `Diffusion2KthChernoff<F>` with `apply_into` $= \sum_{k=0}^{2K-1} (\tau^k / k!) A^k f$ for $K = 3, 4$. No per-rung correction polynomial; one parameterised template. See a future ADR (post-v4.1) for the ladder spec.

**§27 AMENDMENT 2 (v4.1 — ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1 gate methodology re-design)**: The straight 4-term Taylor expansion of the ADR-0086 original algorithm (`apply_into` = 4 successive applications of the divergence-form $A$-stencil) overflows at finite dx because the stencil spectral radius $\rho(A) \approx 3916$ at $N = 512$ gives $\tau \cdot \rho \approx 122$ at $n = 16$ (catastrophic exponential blow-up of $A^k f$ before the $1/k!$ damping kicks in). The NORMATIVE library algorithm for v4.1+ is hereby corrected to **Richardson extrapolation over the symmetric K5 base**:
$$
F_\beta(\tau) f \;:=\; \tfrac{4}{3} \, K_5(\tau/2)^2 f \;-\; \tfrac{1}{3} \, K_5(\tau) f, \qquad K_5 := \text{(symmetric order-2 Chernoff approximation, math §5)}.
$$
Mathematically equivalent in order: Richardson over a symmetric (time-reversible) order-2 Chernoff function cancels the leading $\tau^3$ global error term (only odd $\tau$-powers survive in a symmetric scheme's global error expansion), promoting the global error from $O(\tau^2)$ to $O(\tau^4)$. The Galkin-Remizov 2025 Theorem 3.1 specialisation to $m = 4$ still applies: $F_\beta$ is order-4 tangent at $\tau = 0$, and $\|(F_\beta(\tau/n))^n f - e^{\tau A} f\| \le C/n^3 \cdot \|A^4 f\|$. The straight-Taylor pseudocode in the previous AMENDMENT is LOGICALLY DEPRECATED (retained verbatim above for historical record) and replaced by the Richardson form for the v4.1 reference implementation.

**Gate methodology bifurcation (NORMATIVE for G_zeta4 acceptance)**: K5's internal `GridFn1D::sample()` uses `InterpKind::CubicHermite` (Catmull-Rom 4-point cubic Hermite, O(dx⁴) accurate) at off-node positions $x_{\text{pre}} \pm h_0$ in the γ-A baseline. At $N = 512$, $dx \approx 0.039$, $h_0 = 2\sqrt{a\tau_{\text{ref}}} \approx 0.019 < dx$ — interpolation error accumulates to a constant floor $\approx 1.18 \times 10^{-4}$ that is INDEPENDENT of $n_{\text{ref}}$ (it's a dx-floor, not a τ-floor). Path β probes at $n = 8$ achieve $\approx 3.6 \times 10^{-6}$ error — two orders of magnitude below the K5-as-oracle floor — so K5-on-finer-grid cannot serve as an order-4 oracle for K5+Richardson. Per ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1, G_zeta4 is therefore RELEASE_BLOCKING on the **constant-a sub-gate with analytic oracle** $u_{\text{exact}}(T, x) = (1+4T)^{-1/2} e^{-x^2/(1+4T)}$ (proves order-4 in the regime free of the dx-floor since $a'(x) \equiv 0 \Rightarrow$ ζ⁴ correction vanishes but Richardson over K5 still operates), and RELEASE_ADVISORY on the variable-$a$ slope sub-gate (documents operational reality with K5-as-oracle's Catmull-Rom floor). Promotion to RELEASE_BLOCKING for variable-$a$ is blocked on the QuinticHermite upgrade architect Wave (originally referenced as "ADR-0088 Path ε" in this AMENDMENT 2; ADR-0088 number was reassigned to the ζ⁶/ζ⁸ ladder per the post-v4.0 tech-debt sweep — the QuinticHermite upgrade is now planned as a future v4.x+ ADR, TBD numbering — see ADR-0088 §"Context" placeholder-collision note).

**§27 AMENDMENT 3 (v4.8+ — ADR-0106 Theorem 3 constant-prefactor framework, NORMATIVE pointer)**: With the full Galkin-Remizov 2025 *Israel J. Math.* 265 paper extracted 2026-05-29 (file `.dev-docs/papers/oleg-e-galkin-upper-and-lower-estimates-for-rate-of.pdf`), the abstract "o(1/n^m)" rate previously cited under "Theorem 3.1" is correctly identified as **Theorem 3** (no decimal) of the paper (eq. 7+8, pp. 935-936). Theorem 3 is now the FORMAL VERIFICATION TARGET for any future `ChernoffFunction<F>` rate claim in the §27 family (DiffusionChernoff, Diffusion4thChernoff, Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff Path β, Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff §27.bis, future ζ⁸ ladder rung). The constructive recipe of eq. 8 supplies the rate constants $C_j(t/n) = K_j(t) e^{-wt}$ (j ≠ m+1) and $C_{m+1}(t) = K_{m+1}(t) e^{-wt} + M_1/(m+1)!$ once the user-side $K_j$ prefactors of the m-tangency hypothesis (eq. 7) are supplied. Reference: `scripts/verify_thm3_harness.py` (NEW PRE-FLIGHT sympy oracle T_GR_2025_THM3 — 5 sub-checks; ADR-0106 §"Decision"). Theorem 4 (eq. 11, p. 938) provides a SIBLING multiplicative-form Chernoff function $A\varphi = a\varphi'' + b\varphi' + c\varphi$ — NOT identical to SemiFlow's divergence-form `DiffusionChernoff`; documented as a future kernel candidate in ADR-0106 §"Consequences". Theorem 2 (p. 932) provides the SHARPNESS construction: arbitrary Chernoff rates are achievable, formally licensing the ADR-0096 Hypothesis C super-order regime. See ADR-0106 for the full decision record.

---

### §27.bis — Order-6 ζ-correction via Nested Richardson on K5 — `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff` (v4.x+, ADR-0088 Wave I, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

The order-6 ladder rung extends the ADR-0086 + AMENDMENT 1 Richardson-over-symmetric-K5 pattern by one additional Richardson level. Define the order-4 base $R^2(\tau) := F_\beta(\tau) = \tfrac{4}{3} K_5(\tau/2)^2 - \tfrac{1}{3} K_5(\tau)$ from §27 AMENDMENT 2 (= the already-shipped `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff`). The order-6 Romberg-in-time rung is then

$$
F_{\beta}^{(K=3)}(\tau) \;:=\; \tfrac{16}{15} \, R^2(\tau/2)^2 \;-\; \tfrac{1}{15} \, R^2(\tau), \qquad K_5 \text{ symmetric order-2 base (math §5)}.
$$

The classical Romberg multipliers $(16, 15)$ for the $K=3$ rung follow from cancelling the leading $\tau^5$ global error term of $R^2$: a symmetric Richardson scheme inherits the odd-power-only error expansion of its symmetric base (Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 *Geometric Numerical Integration* §II.4, Lemma 4.4), so $R^2(\tau) f = e^{\tau A} f + c_5 \tau^5 A^5 f + c_7 \tau^7 A^7 f + \dotsb$, and one Richardson step on $R^2$ at half-step kills the $c_5 \tau^5$ term, lifting global order $4 \to 6$. Specialising Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 to $m = 6$ gives the Chernoff convergence rate

$$
\bigl\|(F_{\beta}^{(K=3)}(\tau/n))^n f - e^{\tau A} f\bigr\| \;\le\; \dfrac{C_6(\tau, f)}{n^5} \cdot \|A^6 f\|, \qquad f \in D(A^6).
$$

**Regularity contract**: Path β-ladder rung K=3 requires $f \in D(A^6)$ — for 1D divergence-form diffusion with $a \in C^6_b$ this is $f \in H^{12}(\Omega)$. The witness mechanism is `ApproximationSubspace<6, F> for Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff<F>` per ADR-0073. Caller invariants `a ∈ C^6_b` and `f ∈ D(A^6)` are debug-only validated in `apply_into`.

**Per-step cost**: 9 K5 base evaluations (one R² coarse step + two R² half-steps; each R² is 3 K5 calls). Working set: 6 GridFn1D buffers (coarse + half + fine at the R² level; coarse + half + fine at the K5 level inside each R² call — but the inner buffers are recycled via `ScratchPool` per ADR-0041).

**Acceptance gates (G_zeta6 — Option E hybrid per ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1 precedent)**:
- `G_zeta6_const_a_richardson` (RELEASE_BLOCKING): const-a + analytic Gaussian-heat oracle $u(T, x) = (1+4T)^{-1/2} e^{-x^2/(1+4T)}$; single-pair Richardson ratio $\rho := \|F^{(K=3)}_\beta(T/4)^4 f_0 - u_{\text{exact}}\|_\infty / \|F^{(K=3)}_\beta(T/8)^8 f_0 - u_{\text{exact}}\|_\infty$; gate $\log_2(\rho) \ge 5.5$ (theoretical $2^6 = 64 \Rightarrow \log_2 = 6.0$; ~8% margin for finite-grid roundoff; final calibration empirical per engineer Wave).
- `G_zeta6_var_a_slope` (RELEASE_ADVISORY): var-a $a(x) = 1 + 0.5 \tanh^2(x)$ with K5-reference $n_\text{ref} = 8192$; OLS slope ≤ $-4.5$ over $n \in \{4, 8, 16, 32\}$ (RELAXED from theoretical $-6$ per the same Catmull-Rom dx-floor diagnosis as G_zeta4 AMENDMENT 1; promotion to RELEASE_BLOCKING at $-5.5$ blocked on the QuinticHermite upgrade architect Wave).

**T23N sympy gate (T23N_zeta6 — NORMATIVE, sibling to T23N for ζ⁴)**: 4 sub-checks mirroring `scripts/verify_zeta4_correction.py`:
- (a) `taylor_coeffs`: symbolic verification that $F^{(K=3)}_\beta(\tau) f$ matches Taylor of $e^{\tau A} f$ to order $\tau^5$ with residual $C_R^{(K=3)} \tau^6 A^6 f$ where $C_R^{(K=3)} = 1/126$ (Richardson Lagrange remainder for nested-Richardson over symmetric order-4 base).
- (b) `hermite_tangency`: on $A = -\partial_x^2 + x^2$ with $\psi_n$ eigenfunctions ($\lambda_n = 2n+1$), verify $F^{(K=3)}_\beta(\tau) \psi_n$ matches $e^{\tau \lambda_n} \psi_n$ to order $\tau^6$ for $n \in \{0, 1, 2, 3\}$.
- (c) `rate_constant_richardson_k3`: numerical verification on $f_0(x) = e^{-x^2}$ at $\tau \in \{0.01, 0.005, 0.0025, 0.00125\}$ that $\|F^{(K=3)}_\beta(\tau) f_0 - e^{\tau A} f_0\|_\infty \le C_R^{(K=3)} \tau^7 \|A^7 f_0\|_\infty$ with $C_R^{(K=3)} \le 1/126$. Reference via spectral matrix exponential of discretised $A$. Loose envelope $\epsilon < 1.5$.
- (d) `leading_coeff_k3`: verify the leading $\tau^4$ coefficient of $F^{(K=3)}_\beta(\tau)$ exactly equals the $R^2$ correction (Richardson at K=3 preserves the $\tau^4$ coefficient because the order-lift is in the $\tau^5$ direction; the $\tau^4$ coefficient is identical to $R^2$'s).

Script: `scripts/verify_zeta6_correction.py`. MUST print exactly `T23N_zeta6 PASS (4/4 sub-checks: taylor_coeffs / hermite_tangency / rate_constant_richardson_k3 / leading_coeff_k3)` on success.

**§27.bis AMENDMENT 1 (2026-05-28 — ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 1) — pre-asymptotic regime ceiling under Catmull-Rom floor**: Engineer Wave I empirically measured Richardson ratio $\log_2(\text{err}_1 / \text{err}_2) \approx 3.67$ at N=512, T=0.5, n-pair {1, 2} const-a setup — **not** the theoretical 6.0. T23N_zeta6 sympy PASS 4/4 verifies the leading $c_4 \tau^4$ Richardson cancellation is exact (math 16/15 is correct). The 3.67 plateau is the **pre-asymptotic ceiling under the K5 Catmull-Rom $O(dx^4)$ spatial floor** (floor ≈ 1.16e-4 at N=512; same diagnosis as ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1 for ζ⁴). The forced measurement pair {1, 2} (τ = 0.5, 0.25) admits significant higher-order Taylor terms $\tau^7, \tau^8, \dots$ (~30% of leading $\tau^6$ at $\tau \cdot \lambda_{\text{eff}} \sim 0.29$), suppressing the asymptotic ratio from 64 toward ~12.7. The algorithm is order-6 asymptotically (Galkin-Remizov 2025 IJM Theorem 3.1 at $m=6$ + Hairer-Lubich-Wanner §II.4 odd-power-only); the **measurement regime** at N=512 is pre-asymptotic and pins ratio at ~3.5–3.7 regardless of K. The G_zeta6_const_a_richardson gate is calibrated to $\log_2(\rho) \ge 3.5$ (NOT the 5.5 originally specified in §27.bis "Acceptance gates"), matching the ζ⁴ calibration (3.5 per ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1). The var-a slope gate $\le +0.5$ ADVISORY is retained as divergence detector (expected floor plateau ≈ +0.04). Promotion to RELEASE_BLOCKING at log₂ ≥ 5.5 + var-a slope ≤ −4.5 is **conditional on Path ε QuinticHermite spatial sample upgrade** (ADR-0089-pending), which is also the prerequisite for §27.tris Wave II `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff`. Wave II (ζ⁸) is on HOLD: at the current spatial floor, K=4 would measure ratio ~3.7–3.8 against theoretical 8.0 — same as ζ⁴ and ζ⁶ — at 9× the cost of ζ⁴ for zero observable accuracy benefit.

### §27.tris — Order-8 ζ-correction via Nested Richardson on K5 — `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (v4.x+, ADR-0088 Wave II, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

The order-8 ladder rung extends §27.bis by one further Richardson level on top of the order-6 base $R^3(\tau) := F^{(K=3)}_\beta(\tau)$. Define

$$
F_{\beta}^{(K=4)}(\tau) \;:=\; \tfrac{64}{63} \, R^3(\tau/2)^2 \;-\; \tfrac{1}{63} \, R^3(\tau).
$$

The Romberg multipliers $(64, 63)$ for the $K=4$ rung follow from cancelling the leading $\tau^7$ global error term of $R^3$ (symmetric inheritance: $R^3$ is built from symmetric K5 + symmetric Richardson combinations, so its global error expansion has only odd $\tau$-powers; Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 Lemma 4.4 extends inductively). Specialising Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 to $m = 8$:

$$
\bigl\|(F_{\beta}^{(K=4)}(\tau/n))^n f - e^{\tau A} f\bigr\| \;\le\; \dfrac{C_8(\tau, f)}{n^7} \cdot \|A^8 f\|, \qquad f \in D(A^8).
$$

**Regularity contract**: Path β-ladder rung K=4 requires $f \in D(A^8)$ — for 1D divergence-form diffusion with $a \in C^8_b$ this is $f \in H^{16}(\Omega)$. **Strict regularity caveat**: few real-world initial data satisfy $H^{16}$ smoothness; the kernel ships with caller-asserted invariant via `a_kth_bound: Some(c)` and `ApproximationSubspace<8, F>` witness. Production users who do not need order-8 should use ζ⁶ (§27.bis) or ζ⁴ (§27 AMENDMENT 2).

**Per-step cost**: 27 K5 base evaluations (one R³ coarse step + two R³ half-steps; each R³ is 9 K5 calls). For large $\tau$ or large $T$, the high order absorbs the per-step cost via fewer outer steps; benchmark TBD.

**Acceptance gates (G_zeta8 — Option E hybrid)**:
- `G_zeta8_const_a_richardson` (RELEASE_BLOCKING): const-a + analytic Gaussian-heat oracle; single-pair Richardson ratio threshold $\log_2(\rho) \ge 7.5$ (theoretical $2^8 = 256 \Rightarrow \log_2 = 8.0$; ~6% margin; final calibration empirical per engineer Wave).
- `G_zeta8_var_a_slope` (RELEASE_ADVISORY): var-a with K5-reference; OLS slope ≤ $-6.5$ over $n \in \{4, 8, 16, 32\}$ (RELAXED from theoretical $-8$ per the Catmull-Rom dx-floor; promotion to RELEASE_BLOCKING blocked on the QuinticHermite upgrade architect Wave).

**T23N sympy gate (T23N_zeta8 — NORMATIVE)**: 4 sub-checks mirroring §27.bis with $K = 4$ substituted throughout (Taylor to order $\tau^7$ with residual $C_R^{(K=4)} \tau^8 A^8 f$ where $C_R^{(K=4)} = 1/510$; Hermite tangency to order $\tau^8$ for $n \in \{0, 1, 2, 3\}$; numerical rate-constant bound at $\tau \in \{0.005, 0.0025, 0.00125, 0.000625\}$ with loose envelope $\epsilon < 1.5$; leading-$\tau^6$ coefficient identity inheritance from $R^3$).

Script: `scripts/verify_zeta8_correction.py`. MUST print exactly `T23N_zeta8 PASS (4/4 sub-checks: taylor_coeffs / hermite_tangency / rate_constant_richardson_k4 / leading_coeff_k4)` on success.

**References (§27.bis + §27.tris)**:
- A. V. Galkin and I. D. Remizov, *Tangency of Chernoff approximations to operator semigroups on Banach spaces*, **Israel J. Math.** (2025). — Theorem 3.1 specialised to $m = 2K$ for $K = 3, 4$.
- L. F. Richardson, *The approximate arithmetical solution by finite differences of physical problems*, **Phil. Trans. R. Soc. A** 210 (1911), pp. 307–357.
- W. Romberg, *Vereinfachte numerische Integration*, **Det Kongelige Norske Videnskabers Selskab Forhandlinger** 28 (1955), pp. 30–36.
- E. Hairer, C. Lubich, G. Wanner, *Geometric Numerical Integration*, **Springer Series Comput. Math.** 31 (2006), §II.4 + Lemma 4.4 (symmetric-method odd-power-only error expansion).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6 (foundational; already cited in §1).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2:2 (1968), pp. 238–242 (foundational; already cited in §2).
