**§27.tris AMENDMENT 1 (2026-05-29 — ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 2) — Wave II HOLD-release attempt under Path ε FAILED hard-stop; ζ⁸ DEFERRED to v4.3+**: Following ADR-0089 AMENDMENT 1 landing (Path ε ζ⁶-only Quintic K5 wiring) the Wave II HOLD was provisionally lifted and engineer ran the Wave II calibration measurement. T23N_zeta8 sympy PASS 4/4 verifies the 64/63 Richardson cancellation symbolically (algorithm wiring correct). Empirical measurement at canonical setup (N=512, T=0.5, n-pair {1, 2}, const-a) returned $\log_2(\text{err}_1/\text{err}_2) = 3.067$ — **below** the §27.bis ζ⁶ measurement 3.868 (a regression in K) and below the §27.tris "Acceptance gates" §"Risk note" hard-stop floor of 4.0. Architectural diagnosis: at $\tau = 0.5$ on the canonical setup, the inner $R^3$'s pre-asymptotic residuals are large enough that the outer Richardson $K=4$ layer *cancels* $c_8 \tau^8$ terms it cannot actually reach yet; meanwhile at $n = 2$ ($\tau = 0.25$) the Quintic K5 spatial floor (~$10^{-6}$) is already encroaching, contaminating the n-pair {1, 2} ratio with floor effects. This is a **floor-cascade regime** distinct from (and deeper than) the Catmull-Rom regime ceiling that capped §27 + §27.bis at 3.5 / 3.8: nesting a 4th Richardson rung at the same pre-asymptotic $\tau$ amplifies floor effects monotonically with K rather than cancelling temporal error, violating monotonic order improvement at the measurement scale. **Decision**: ship `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff` at v4.2; defer `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` to v4.3+ ADR-0090 pending architectural advance (3 mutually-compatible investigation directions: SepticHermite spatial sample lifting floor to $10^{-10}$; Romberg-2D direct algorithm eliminating intermediate Richardson layers; or larger-N measurement window N $\in \{1024, 2048\}$ creating measurable-$\tau$ regime down to $\tau \approx 10^{-4}$). The asymptotic Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 at $m = 8$ result above is mathematically unchanged (the algorithm IS order-8 in the asymptotic regime); only the v4.2 **measurement regime** at N=512 with current Quintic floor cannot exhibit it. Wave II spec preserved as research artifact under `.dev-docs/research/zeta8-wave-ii-deferred.md` (engineer creates from uncommitted sources per ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 2 §"Engineer guidance"). See ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 2 for full rationale; v4.3+ ADR-0090 for the investigation roadmap.

---

### §27.quart — Order-8 ζ-correction via diagonal Padé P₄/Q₄ on K5 — `Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` (v4.3+, ADR-0091, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

Direct order-8 alternative to the DEFERRED §27.tris nested Richardson rung. The diagonal Padé approximant of `exp(z)` at degree $K = 4$ achieves order $2K = 8$ in a single step via rational approximation rather than recursive cascade:

$$
\frac{P_4(z)}{Q_4(z)} \;=\; \exp(z) \;+\; \mathcal{O}(z^9), \qquad
\begin{aligned}
P_4(z) &= 1 + \tfrac{1}{2} z + \tfrac{3}{28} z^2 + \tfrac{1}{84} z^3 + \tfrac{1}{1680} z^4, \\
Q_4(z) &= 1 - \tfrac{1}{2} z + \tfrac{3}{28} z^2 - \tfrac{1}{84} z^3 + \tfrac{1}{1680} z^4 \;=\; P_4(-z).
\end{aligned}
$$

Coefficients are classical from the Padé table (Baker-Graves-Morris 1996 *Padé Approximants* §1.2 verbatim; equivalently Higham 2005 *SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl.* Table 2.3 row $m = 4$). The $Q$-as-mirror-image-of-$P$ property $Q_4(z) = P_4(-z)$ yields the unitarity-preserving Cayley-style structure observed for diagonal Padé in Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 §3.4 Theorem 3.5.

**Algorithm (NORMATIVE library; canonical Higham 2005 algorithm without scaling-and-squaring at the v4.3 baseline)**: for each outer step of size $\tau$ on input `src`, compute:

```text
Step 1 — assemble RHS via 4 sequential A-stencil applications:
  A_src   = A · src                              (apply_div_form helper, reused from §27.bis)
  A2_src  = A · A_src
  A3_src  = A · A2_src
  A4_src  = A · A3_src
  rhs[i]  = src[i] + (τ/2)·A_src[i]
                   + (3·τ²/28)·A2_src[i]
                   + (τ³/84)·A3_src[i]
                   + (τ⁴/1680)·A4_src[i]

Step 2 — assemble Q_4(τA) as 9-banded matrix B of size N×N:
  B = I − (τ/2)·A_mat + (3·τ²/28)·A_mat² − (τ³/84)·A_mat³ + (τ⁴/1680)·A_mat⁴
  where A_mat is the 3-banded discrete divergence-form stencil (Neumann BCs);
  B has bandwidth 2K+1 = 9 (polynomial-of-tridiagonal yields band 2·deg + 1).

Step 3 — solve B · dst = rhs via banded LU with partial pivoting:
  O(N · K²) factor + O(N · K) back-solve ≈ 8200 flops at N=512, K=4.
  Algorithm template: Golub-Van Loan §4.5 (banded LU); implementation mirrors
  v4.1 matrix_strang.rs block-Thomas at scalar level (sub/sup arrays of length
  N − k for k = 1..4; main of length N; partial pivoting for stability).
```

**Convergence (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 specialised to $m = 8$, generalised to rational approximation per Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 §3.4)**:

$$
\bigl\|(F_{\text{Padé}}^{(K=4)}(\tau/n))^n f - e^{\tau A} f\bigr\| \;\le\; \dfrac{C_8^{\text{Padé}}(\tau, f)}{n^7} \cdot \|A^8 f\|, \qquad f \in D(A^8),
$$

where $C_8^{\text{Padé}}$ inherits the Padé Lagrange remainder constant from Higham 2005 Lemma 2.1 (scalar bound; generalises to operator A via spectral mapping for $\rho(\tau A) < 5.4$ per Higham 2005 Table 2.1).

**Regularity contract**: Path Padé rung K=4 requires $f \in D(A^8)$ — same contract as §27.tris nested Richardson; for 1D divergence-form diffusion with $a \in C^8_b$ this is $f \in H^{16}(\Omega)$. **Strict regularity caveat**: few real-world initial data satisfy $H^{16}$ smoothness; the kernel ships with caller-asserted invariant via `a_kth_bound: Some(c)` and `ApproximationSubspace<8, F>` witness. Production users who do not need order-8 should use ζ⁶ (§27.bis) or ζ⁴ (§27 AMENDMENT 2).

**Per-step cost**: 8 A-stencil applications + one 9-banded LU factor + back-solve ≈ **8-9× K5 cost per outer τ-step**. Compare to DEFERRED §27.tris nested Richardson: 27× K5 cost per step. Padé is **~3× cheaper** at K=4 while bypassing the floor-cascade regime (no recursive Richardson nesting → no nested floor amplification).

**Stability**: unconditionally stable for any $\tau > 0$ when A is dissipative (real spectrum $\le 0$ — divergence-form heat with Neumann BCs satisfies this). Diagonal Padé preserves A-stability per Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 §3.4 Theorem 3.5.

**Scaling-and-squaring deferred at v4.3 baseline**: Higham 2005's full algorithm includes scaling $\tau A \to \tau A / 2^s$ to bound spectral radius then squaring $R(\tau A)^{2^s}$ to recover $\exp(\tau A)$. For our v4.3 use case at N=512 with $\tau \le 0.5$ and K5 stencil spectral radius $\rho \approx 3916$, direct $\tau \cdot \rho$ exceeds the Padé degree-4 convergence radius ($\sim 5.4$ per Higham 2005 Table 2.1); the Chernoff outer loop $(F(\tau/n))^n$ for $n \ge 32$ implicitly scales $\tau_{\text{inner}} = \tau/n \le 0.016$. Add explicit scaling-and-squaring infrastructure ONLY if `G_zeta8_pade_const_a_richardson` calibration fails the Wave I gate; documented in ADR-0091 as conditional follow-up.

**Acceptance gates (Option E hybrid per ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1 precedent)**:
- `G_zeta8_pade_const_a_richardson` (RELEASE_BLOCKING): const-a + analytic Gaussian-heat oracle $u(T, x) = (1+4T)^{-1/2} e^{-x^2/(1+4T)}$; single-pair Richardson ratio $\rho := \|F_{\text{Padé}}^{(K=4)}(T/4)^4 f_0 - u_{\text{exact}}\|_\infty / \|F_{\text{Padé}}^{(K=4)}(T/8)^8 f_0 - u_{\text{exact}}\|_\infty$; gate $\log_2(\rho) \ge 5.5$ initial (theoretical $2^8 = 256 \Rightarrow \log_2 = 8.0$; calibration empirical per engineer Wave per ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 1 hybrid rule: measured ratio $\to \lfloor \log_2(\text{ratio}) - 0.1 \rfloor + 0.1$ rounded to one decimal).
- `G_zeta8_pade_var_a_slope` (RELEASE_ADVISORY): var-a $a(x) = 1 + 0.5 \tanh^2(x)$ with K5-reference $n_\text{ref} = 8192$; OLS slope $\le -6.5$ over $n \in \{4, 8, 16, 32\}$ (RELAXED from theoretical $-8$ per the Catmull-Rom dx-floor; promotion to RELEASE_BLOCKING $\le -7.5$ blocked on the QuinticHermite / Chebyshev spectral spatial upgrade).

**T_ZETA8_PADE sympy gate (NORMATIVE)**: 4 sub-checks:
- (a) `pade_identity`: symbolic verification that $P_4(z) - \exp(z) \cdot Q_4(z) = \mathcal{O}(z^9)$ as a scalar power series in $z$ (sympy `series(expr, z, 0, 10)` returns residual leading-term coefficient $\ge 10^{-15}$ at order $z^9$ and exactly zero at orders $z^0$ through $z^8$).
- (b) `hermite_tangency`: on $A = -\partial_x^2 + x^2$ with $\psi_n$ eigenfunctions ($\lambda_n = 2n+1$), verify $F_{\text{Padé}}^{(K=4)}(\tau) \psi_n$ matches $e^{\tau \lambda_n} \psi_n$ to order $\tau^8$ for $n \in \{0, 1, 2, 3\}$.
- (c) `rate_constant_pade`: numerical verification on $f_0(x) = e^{-x^2}$ at $\tau \in \{0.005, 0.0025, 0.00125, 0.000625\}$ that $\|F_{\text{Padé}}^{(K=4)}(\tau) f_0 - e^{\tau A} f_0\|_\infty \le C_8^{\text{Padé}} \tau^9 \|A^9 f_0\|_\infty$ with $C_8^{\text{Padé}} \le 1/117600$.
- (d) `q4_invertibility`: confirm $Q_4(\tau \lambda_n) \ne 0$ for all Hermite eigenvalues at canonical $\tau \in \{0.001, 0.01, 0.1, 0.5\}$ (sanity check that banded LU never encounters singular pivot under dissipative A).

Script: `scripts/verify_zeta8_pade.py`. MUST print exactly `T_ZETA8_PADE PASS (4/4 sub-checks: pade_identity / hermite_tangency / rate_constant_pade / q4_invertibility)` on success.

**References (§27.quart, additional to those in §27.bis + §27.tris)**:
- N. J. Higham (2005), *The Scaling and Squaring Method for the Matrix Exponential Revisited*, **SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl.** 26(4), pp. 1179-1193 — canonical scale-and-square Padé algorithm; we use the Padé component without scaling at the v4.3 baseline (calibration measurement determines need for follow-up scaling).
- M. Hochbruck, C. Lubich (2010), *Exponential integrators*, **Acta Numerica** 19, pp. 209-286, §3.4 (A-stability of Cayley-style rational approximations; generalises matrix Padé to operator semigroup setting).
- G. A. Baker, P. Graves-Morris (1996), *Padé Approximants*, **Cambridge University Press** §1.2 (classical Padé table for `exp(z)`; P_4/Q_4 coefficients verbatim).
- G. H. Golub, C. F. Van Loan (1996), *Matrix Computations* 3rd ed., **Johns Hopkins University Press** §4.5 (banded LU with partial pivoting; algorithm template for `banded_lu.rs` sibling module).
- ADR-0091 — engineer Wave I spec (`Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` + `banded_lu` sibling module); `.dev-docs/specs/pade-zeta8-wave.md`.

#### §27.quart AMENDMENT 1 (2026-05-29) — Operator-level kernel `Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` DEFERRED to v4.4+; scalar Padé identity preserved as CITATION mathematics

The classical Padé identity `P_4(z)/Q_4(z) = exp(z) + O(z^9)` (Baker-Graves-Morris 1996 §1.2) is unconditionally correct as scalar mathematics and is verified by `T_ZETA8_PADE` sympy oracle 4/4 PASS. The Wave I engineer implementation `Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` instantiated this identity on the discretised K5 operator `A` *without* the canonical Higham 2005 scaling-and-squaring envelope: at `N=512` on `[−10, 10]` the operator norm is `‖A‖₂ ≈ 2.6 · 10^5`, so even at `n = 32` (canonical Chernoff outer loop) `τ_inner · ‖A‖ ≈ 62`, far above the Padé degree-4 convergence radius `~5.4` per Higham 2005 Table 2.1. The Wave I calibration measurement returned `log₂(err_4/err_8) = 7.87` (above the 7.0 placeholder threshold) but with absolute errors `≈ 4.97 · 10^{31}` — both numerator and denominator dominated by the same `1/‖A‖^{28} · τ^8` polynomial blow-up; the ratio is algebraically correct while absolute values are meaningless. The operator-level kernel is therefore DEFERRED to v4.4+ per ADR-0091 AMENDMENT 1 (Option γ); the §27.quart algorithm specification stays in math.md as CITATION mathematics (no normative library mapping at v4.3+) until the v4.4+ follow-up ADR adds the full Higham 2005 algorithm (1-norm spectral-radius estimator + Algorithm 2.3 scaling-parameter selection + squaring loop with accumulator guards). The order-8 ζ⁸ contract is closed at v4.3 via §27.tris-resurrected `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (nested Richardson on Quintic-K5 with default-ON Chebyshev spatial floor lift per ADR-0090 / §9.2.7); see ADR-0090 §"ζ⁸ Wave II RESURRECTION". `G_zeta8_pade_const_a_richardson_ratio` + `G_zeta8_pade_var_a_temporal_slope` are RETIRED from `properties.yaml` at v4.3; they re-enter scope only with the v4.4+ scaling-and-squaring revival. Research artifact preserving the Wave B source/test/sympy + bug-fixer diagnosis + measurement record: `.dev-docs/research/zeta8-pade-wave-b-deferred.md`.

#### §27.quart AMENDMENT 2 (2026-05-29) — Scaling-and-squaring envelope lifts deferral; `Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` REVIVED at v4.4+ per ADR-0094 (NORMATIVE algorithm specification)

The v4.4+ research wave located N. J. Higham (2005) *SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl.* 26(4) pp. 1179-1193 as a FREE PDF (Manchester eprints, DOI 10.1137/04061101X), supplying the missing scaling-and-squaring envelope that AMENDMENT 1 identified as the v4.4+ unblocker. ADR-0094 (Option I) adopts the canonical Higham 2005 algorithm at Padé degree m=4 (reusing the Wave B `banded_lu.rs` bandwidth-9 helper verbatim per suckless minimisation against Higham's no-scaling m=13 default — see ADR-0094 §"Algorithm" `degree choice`). The NORMATIVE algorithm appended to §27.quart is: (1) estimate `ν := τ · ‖A‖_∞` via the 1-norm power-iteration estimator of Higham 2002 §15.3 Algorithm 4.1 with deterministic seed (3-5 iterations sufficient at our N ≤ 2048 scope, ~5 K5-equivalent stencil applications); (2) select `s := max(0, ⌈log₂(ν / θ_4)⌉)` where `θ_4 = 5.4` is the Padé-degree-4 convergence radius (Higham 2005 Table 2.1), ensuring the post-scaling invariant `τ_scaled · ‖A‖_∞ ≤ θ_4` where `τ_scaled := τ / 2^s`; (3) compute the base Padé approximation `half := Q_4(τ_scaled · A)^{-1} · P_4(τ_scaled · A) · src` via Wave B's verbatim algorithm (4 sequential A-applications for P_4 RHS + banded LU solve for Q_4); (4) square `s` times: `for i in 1..=s: half := apply_into(τ_scaled · 2^i, half, scratch)`. At N=512, τ=0.125, ‖A‖_∞ ≈ 2.6·10^5: `ν ≈ 3.25·10^4`, `s = ⌈log₂(6019)⌉ = 13`, total cost ≈ 125-135× K5 per outer step (5 estimator + 9 Padé base + 13×9 squaring) — competitive with the v4.3 Chebyshev ζ⁸ kernel's ~576 flops per grid per stencil (M=64 virtual-node QuinticHermite × 9 sample calls per stencil). Stability per Higham 2005 §2.5 + Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 §3.4: each squaring step satisfies `‖R(τ_scaled · 2^{i-1} · A)‖ ≤ 1 + ε` for dissipative `A` (heat operator with Neumann BCs has `Re(σ(A)) ≤ 0`); accumulated rounding error bounded by `s · u + O(u^2)`. Acceptance gates `G_zeta8_pade_const_a_richardson_ratio` + `G_zeta8_pade_var_a_temporal_slope` are RE-ENTERED to `properties.yaml` at v4.4+ (calibrated per Option E hybrid rule); 1 NEW envelope gate `G_PADE_SS_NORM_ENVELOPE` verifies the post-scaling invariant `τ_scaled · ‖A‖_∞ ≤ 5.4` BLOCKING. T_ZETA8_PADE sympy oracle gains 1 NEW sub-check `s_selection_rule` verifying the `⌈log₂⌉` formula symbolically (preserves 4/4 PASS from Wave B + 1/1 NEW = 5/5 total). Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff becomes a v4.4 **alternative** ζ⁸ kernel coexisting with the v4.3 Chebyshev `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` (suckless third-occurrence test passes per ADR-0094 §"Rationale" — distinct A-stability + var-coef-directness regimes). Dec 2025 arXiv:2512.20777 Padé+Taylor hybrid (2.6× speedup via Sastre-Ibáñez-Defez 3-mat-mult Taylor) DEFERRED to v4.5+ ADR-0094 follow-up per `.dev-docs/research/verdicts/verdict-v4-4-research-wave.md` §user-attention #3 ("actively-evolving research frontier; monitor for 2026 follow-ups before committing").

#### §27.quart AMENDMENT 3 (2026-05-29) — TERMINAL CLOSURE per ADR-0101 (v5.0 third-attempt FAILED PRE-FLIGHT for all of Path α/β/γ); Padé operator-level kernel permanently DEFERRED v6.0+ pending external math advance; ζ⁸ contract remains closed via §27.tris Chebyshev `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` ALONE

AMENDMENT 2 above lifted the v4.3 deferral conditionally on a v4.4+ engineer wave (Wave I per ADR-0094 §"Implementation cost estimate"). The Wave I landing at v4.5 RE-DEFERRED per ADR-0094 AMENDMENT 1 with const-a Richardson ratio `log₂ = −0.4053` (anti-convergent) despite the scaling-and-squaring envelope gate `G_PADE_SS_NORM_ENVELOPE` PASSING — diagnosed as one of {D1 P₄/Q₄ coefficient transcription bug, D2 banded-LU error propagation under repeated squaring, D3 scalar-vs-matrix squaring mismatch per Higham 2005 §2.5}. D3 was rated MOST PLAUSIBLE on architectural grounds and was the binding constraint that ADR-0094 AMENDMENT 1 §"v5.0+ follow-up directions" earmarked for v5.0 third-attempt resolution via "(1) Genuine matrix-squaring loop (~400 LoC)" alongside m=13 (Path β) and Krylov-Arnoldi (Path γ) alternatives.

ADR-0101 PRE-FLIGHT sympy (`/tmp/pade_v5_preflight.py`, executed 2026-05-29) **FALSIFIES** the D3 hypothesis: for a fixed Padé operator $R := Q_4(τ_{\text{scaled}} A)^{-1} \cdot P_4(τ_{\text{scaled}} A)$ on a symbolic 3×3 dissipative test operator $A = \mathrm{trid}(-2, 1)$, the matrix power $R^{2^s}$ computed via genuine matrix-matrix squaring and the vector iteration $R \cdot R \cdots R \cdot v$ (Wave I's `apply_into` chained $2^s$ times) produce results agreeing to within $1 \cdot \mathrm{ULP}_{64}$ (measured $\|v_{\text{iter}} - v_{\text{explicit}}\|_1 = 0.000 \cdot 10^0$ at $s = 2$). The Higham 2005 §2.5 warning against scalar-vs-matrix confusion applies to scaling-and-squaring formulas where $R$ ITSELF depends on the iteration step (e.g., a per-step recomputed $R_k = R(τ / 2^k \cdot A)$ family) — it does NOT apply to the Wave I pattern where $R$ is fixed at $τ_{\text{scaled}}$ and iterated. Wave I anti-convergence was therefore D1 or D2 (coefficient transcription or banded-LU floor accumulation), NOT D3. **Path α is mathematically equivalent to Wave I**: a v5.0+ genuine matrix-squaring rewrite would produce byte-identical numerics and inherit the same anti-convergence.

Path β (Higham $m = 13$) PRE-FLIGHT: $\theta_{13} = 5.371920\ldots$ vs $\theta_4 = 5.4$ differ by ${\approx} 0.5\%$; the squaring depth $s = \max(0, \lceil \log_2(\nu / \theta_m) \rceil)$ rounds to identical integers across all $N \in \{128, 256, 512, 1024, 2048\}$ for the canonical Chernoff setup ($N = 512$ canonical: $s_4 = 1$, $s_{13} = 1$; $N = 2048$: $s_4 = 5$, $s_{13} = 5$). The ${\sim}600$ LoC bandwidth-27 `banded_lu_m13.rs` helper (per ADR-0094 §"Degree choice m=4 vs Higham 2005's m=13") and Cohort 11 carve-out would purchase ZERO envelope advantage and inherit the same D1/D2 defect. Path γ (Krylov-Arnoldi minimal Saad 1992) is architecturally eligible under the constitution v1.8.0 3/3 dep cap (hand-rolled = no 4th dep) but the Hessenberg matrix-exp step is the SAME Padé primitive at smaller scale ($k \times k$ for $k \leq 30$), creating a circular dependency — if Path α fails on $N \times N$ due to D1/D2, the same defect inherits to the $k \times k$ Hessenberg matrix-exp.

**TERMINAL CLOSURE (NORMATIVE)**: per ADR-0101 §"Decision", the Padé operator-level kernel `Diffusion8thZeta8PadeChernoff` is permanently DEFERRED to v6.0+ pending external mathematical advance. The ζ⁸ NORMATIVE library kernel for v4.3+ through v5.x+ is `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` per §27.tris (nested Richardson on Quintic-K5 with default-ON Chebyshev spatial floor lift, ADR-0090) ALONE. The §27.quart algorithm specification (AMENDMENT 2's NORMATIVE algorithm) is hereby DOWNGRADED back to CITATION mathematics (no normative library mapping at v5.x+) — the scalar Padé identity $P_4(z)/Q_4(z) = e^z + \mathcal{O}(z^9)$ + Higham 2005 scaling-and-squaring envelope remain mathematically correct as algorithmic background, but no library kernel implements them through v5.x+. The retired acceptance gates `G_zeta8_pade_const_a_richardson_ratio` + `G_zeta8_pade_var_a_temporal_slope` + `G_PADE_SS_NORM_ENVELOPE` and the `T_ZETA8_PADE` sympy oracle stay RETIRED through v5.x+ pending v6.0+ revival. v6.0+ revival requires PRE-FLIGHT clearance of an α/β/γ-equivalent path AND citation to a published algorithm demonstrating Wave-I-bug-bypass (e.g., a Sastre-Ibáñez-Defez 2025+ follow-up resolving the scalar-vs-matrix-iteration equivalence in a manner that admits Wave-I-class implementations). Research artifacts preserved: `.dev-docs/research/zeta8-pade-wave-b-deferred.md` (Wave B v4.3) and `.dev-docs/research/zeta8-pade-wave-i-revival-deferred.md` (Wave I v4.5 + ADR-0101 final-closure marker appended per Deliverable 3 of ADR-0101).

---

### §27.quint — Romberg-2D Operator Semigroup Extrapolation — NEGATIVE RESULT, Outcome B (v4.3+, ADR-0092, NOT IMPLEMENTED; research deliverable only)

Per user directive "если не найдёшь, попробуй сам создать математику" (Wave 2 research synthesis in `.dev-docs/research/raw-findings-romberg-2d.md` confirmed no published Romberg-2D for operator semigroup approximation; 61 sources, 0 direct hits), the architect attempted to derive a 2D extrapolation table for the (τ refinement × K cascade depth) grid that would extract order $2K$ convergence DIRECTLY from K5 base samples without intermediate Richardson stages — hypothesised to bypass the floor-cascade contamination diagnosed in §27.tris AMENDMENT 2 (ζ⁸ Wave II DEFER per ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 2).

**Construction (NORMATIVE, per sympy derivation in `scripts/derive_romberg_2d.py`)**: define the SYMMETRIC composed approximation $U(h) := K5(h)^{T/h}$ (composition of $n = T/h$ K5 steps to reach final time $T$). Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 Theorem II.4.7 (symmetric methods have even-power-only global error) gives $U(h) = e^{TA} + a_2 h^2 + a_4 h^4 + a_6 h^6 + a_8 h^8 + \mathcal{O}(h^{10})$. Build the Romberg table

$$
T[0, m] := U(h / 2^m), \qquad T[j, m] := \frac{4^j \cdot T[j-1, m+1] - T[j-1, m]}{4^j - 1},
$$

for $j = 0, \ldots, K$ and $m = 0, \ldots, K - j$. The final extrapolant $T[K, 0]$ achieves order $2(K+1)$ accuracy at the cost of $K+1$ INDEPENDENT base trajectories $U(h/2^0), U(h/2^1), \ldots, U(h/2^K)$.

**Sympy verification (4 sub-checks in `scripts/derive_romberg_2d.py`)**:

| Sub-check | Result |
|---|---|
| (a) Symmetric-base error structure | Structural assumption from HLW 2006 Thm II.4.7; scalar surrogate confirms asymmetric/symmetric distinction. |
| (b) Table construction order-lift | **PASS** — $T[j, 0]$ kills error terms $h^2, h^4, \ldots, h^{2j}$, leaving leading $h^{2(j+1)}$. Math is mathematically correct. |
| (c) **Algebraic equivalence to nested Richardson** | **PROVED EXACT**: $T[2, 0] - R^3(h) = 0$ for the K=2 (order 6) case computed symbolically. The two schemes are TWO DIFFERENT BOOKKEEPING SCHEDULES for the SAME unique linear combination of base samples. |
| (d) Floor contamination model | At single outer step (n_outer = 1), the floor amplification $\bigl|\sum_m w_m^{(K)} \cdot 2^m\bigr|$ is identical for both algorithms (because the algorithms ARE identical). For $K = 3$: $w_m = \{-1/2835, 4/135, -64/135, 4096/2835\}$, $|w|_{L^1} = 1105/567$, floor amp $= 3937/405 \approx 9.72$. |

**Conclusion (Outcome B; NORMATIVE library-scope decision)**: the Romberg-2D scheme is mathematically sound (order-correct) but is **EXACTLY ALGEBRAICALLY EQUIVALENT** to the nested Richardson cascade $R^{K+1}$ from §27.bis / §27.tris at the single-outer-step regime that is the relevant ζ⁸ Wave II measurement scale. The polynomial-elimination problem at $K+1$ nodes has a UNIQUE solution; both the nested Richardson recurrence and the Romberg table recurrence compute the same final linear combination. Therefore Romberg-2D **does NOT bypass** the floor-cascade contamination — the floor problem is intrinsic to the spatial discretisation (Catmull-Rom $\mathcal{O}(dx^4)$ sample floor per §27.bis AMENDMENT 1 / §27.tris AMENDMENT 1), not to the temporal extrapolation scheme.

**Genuine novelty pathways** (none scheduled at v4.3+; documented for v5.x+ research): (1) non-power-of-2 step refinements (Bulirsch-Stoer sequence); (2) non-linear acceleration on the sequence $T[j, 0]$ (Wynn $\varepsilon$-algorithm); (3) rational extrapolation (Bulirsch-Stoer 1966) instead of polynomial; (4) genuinely DIFFERENT paradigm — diagonal Padé $P_4/Q_4$ scaling-and-squaring per §27.quart, which IS scheduled at v4.3+ as ADR-0091 and is mathematically distinct from any Romberg-style cascade. Per `verdict-v4-3-research-waves.md` Priority 1 the binding constraint is the SPATIAL floor, addressable by Chebyshev spectral collocation (v4.3+ ADR-0090 candidate); per Priority 2 the direct ζ⁸ alternative is diagonal Padé (v4.3+ ADR-0091 candidate). Romberg-2D is FORECLOSED per this section.

**No acceptance gate, no kernel, no schema bump** — research deliverable only. Sympy script `scripts/derive_romberg_2d.py` ships alongside `verify_zeta6_correction.py` etc. (not added to T23N suite; `ROMBERG_2D PASS — Outcome B` is the artifact's self-reporting line on successful run).

**References (§27.quint, additional to those in §27.bis + §27.tris + §27.quart)**:
- L. F. Richardson (1911), *The approximate arithmetical solution by finite differences of physical problems*, **Phil. Trans. R. Soc. A** 210, pp. 307-357 — extrapolation foundation; the K=1 case of the present table.
- W. Romberg (1955), *Vereinfachte numerische Integration*, **Det Kongelige Norske Videnskabers Selskab Forhandlinger** 28, pp. 30-36 — classical Romberg integration table; the structural template adopted in the present construction.
- R. Bulirsch, J. Stoer (1966), *Numerical treatment of ordinary differential equations by extrapolation methods*, **Numerische Mathematik** 8(1), pp. 1-13 — extrapolation algorithms for ODE; Bulirsch-Stoer sequence is the v5.x+ genuine-novelty pathway (1) above.
- E. Hairer, C. Lubich, G. Wanner (2006), *Geometric Numerical Integration* 2nd ed., **Springer SCM** 31, §II.4 + §II.9 (Romberg-in-time for symmetric methods; Theorem II.4.7 even-power error structural assumption).
- ADR-0092 — this section's authority; research deliverable + sympy script + verdict.
- `scripts/derive_romberg_2d.py` — sympy verification with 4 sub-checks.
- `.dev-docs/research/verdicts/verdict-romberg-2d-attempt.md` — verdict artifact (negative result with re-route to Path ε / Padé).
- `.dev-docs/research/raw-findings-romberg-2d.md` — Wave 2 research (61 sources reviewed).

### §27 LINEAGE NOTE (v4.4+ — ADR-0093 attribution correction)

The v3.0 ζ⁴ "6-monomial polynomial $P_2[A]$ with leading $-1/12$" construction (originally §27.2 + §27.3) was a v3.0 engineering hypothesis; ADR-0075's attribution to *Galkin-Remizov 2025 Israel J. Math.* Example 4.2 has been **RETRACTED** via full PDF verification (2026-05-29; ADR-0093, extract `.dev-docs/research/extracts/galkin-remizov-2025-extract.md`). The cited Example 4.2 eq. (33) is a 4-shift order-1 tangent kernel for $Au = a u'' + b u' + c u$; its residual bound eq. (34) is the 2-term Lagrange remainder $\|S(t) f - (f + tAf)\| \le t^2 ( (2/3) \|a\|^2 \|f^{IV}\| + \|b\|^2 \|f''\| )$ — no 6-monomial polynomial appears anywhere in the paper. Theorem 3.1 (paper pp. 18-19) is an abstract rate-of-convergence theorem $\|S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f\| \le (C\,t^{m+1}/n^m)\sum K_j\|L^j f\|$ conditional on user-supplied $m$-tangency; it does not *construct* high-order Chernoff functions, it only states $O(n^{-m})$ convergence *if* an $m$-tangent $S(t)$ is supplied. The validated v4.1 Path β Richardson approach (ADR-0086 + AMENDMENT 1) descends from Vedenin et al. 2020 *Math. Notes* 108(3) (canonical Remizov ApproximationSubspace framework, $k=1$ $G(t)$ + $k=2$ $S(t)$) / Remizov 2018 *Appl. Math. Comput.* 328 (`DiffusionChernoff::new` direct lineage) / Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* abstract Theorem 3.1 (the $m=4$ specialisation guarantees the asymptotic rate). The ζ⁴/ζ⁶/ζ⁸ ladder genuine novelty is CONFIRMED across 4 independent extracts + knowledge-fetcher 2010-2026 sweep — no published Chernoff order-6/8 kernels exist outside the SemiFlow ζ-ladder (no SWW prior art; Shamarova-Smolyanov-Weizsäcker-Wittich caps at order-1 tangency). See `.dev-docs/research/verdicts/verdict-v4-4-research-wave.md` §Q4 for the full synthesis.

---

## §28 — Hörmander hypoelliptic Chernoff approximation (v3.1, ADR-0077, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §28.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v0.x–v3.0 elliptic, manifold, and graph kernels all assume the generator $L$ is *elliptic* in the relevant directions: the principal symbol $\sigma_L(\xi) \ne 0$ for $\xi \ne 0$ in the appropriate (cotangent / discrete) sense. Hörmander 1967 *Acta Math.* showed that a strictly weaker class — **hypoelliptic operators** of the form $L = X_0 + \tfrac{1}{2} \sum_{k=1}^{M} X_k^2$ where $\{X_i\}$ are smooth vector fields satisfying the **bracket-generating condition** — admit smooth semigroups even when the principal symbol degenerates. The Festschrift §3 open problem asks whether the Chernoff product formula admits a *constructive* hypoelliptic approximant.

v3.1 ships `HypoellipticChernoff<F, D, M>` — the **first** peer-reviewable Rust implementation of a hypoelliptic Chernoff approximation — via the palindromic Strang-Hörmander decomposition, order-2 tangent on $D(L^2)$ for step-2 Carnot groups (Kolmogorov 1934, Heisenberg group). The order-2 tangency rides on v3.0's `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` witness (ADR-0073 / math.md §26). Higher orders (K ≥ 3) and step ≥ 3 Carnot groups remain OPEN math (Festschrift §3) — explicitly cited in the publication track (`docs/papers/hormander-paper-draft.md`).

### §28.2 — Hörmander 1967 bracket-generating condition (CITATION — *Acta Math.* §1)

**Definition 28.1 (bracket-generating condition).** Let $\{X_0, X_1, \ldots, X_M\}$ be smooth vector fields on a smooth manifold $M$ of dimension $D$. The collection is **bracket-generating** at $x \in M$ if the Lie algebra generated by iterated brackets of the $X_i$ spans the tangent space:
$$
\text{Lie}_x(X_0, X_1, \ldots, X_M) := \text{span}\bigl\{ X_i(x),\ [X_i, X_j](x),\ [X_i, [X_j, X_k]](x),\ \ldots \bigr\} \;=\; T_x M. \tag{28.1}
$$

**Definition 28.2 (step).** The **step** at $x$ is the smallest integer $r \ge 1$ such that iterated brackets up to depth $r$ already span $T_x M$. Step 1 means $\{X_i\}$ themselves span (elliptic case); step 2 means brackets $[X_i, X_j]$ suffice; step 3 means $[X_i, [X_j, X_k]]$ is needed; etc.

**Theorem 28.1 (Hörmander 1967 *Acta Math.* §1, Theorem 1.1 specialised to second-order operators).** If $\{X_0, X_1, \ldots, X_M\}$ is bracket-generating at every $x \in M$, the operator
$$
L = X_0 + \tfrac{1}{2} \sum_{k=1}^{M} X_k^2 \tag{28.2}
$$
is **hypoelliptic**: every distributional solution $u$ of $Lu = f$ with $f \in C^\infty$ is itself $C^\infty$.

**Proof reference**: Hörmander 1967 *Acta Math.* §1.4 (the geometric argument via Hörmander's sum-of-squares regularity proof). The library reproduces only the STATEMENT; the proof lives in the cited paper.

**Kolmogorov 1934 fundamental solution (canonical step-2 example, CITATION — *Math. Annalen* equation 5)**: on $M = \mathbb{R}^2 = \{(x, v)\}$ with $X_0 = v \cdot \partial_x$ and $X_1 = \partial_v$, the operator $L = X_0 + \tfrac{1}{2} X_1^2 = v \partial_x + \tfrac{1}{2} \partial_v^2$ is bracket-generating at step 2 (the bracket $[X_1, X_0] = \partial_x$ supplies the missing direction). The fundamental solution $p(t, x, v ; x_0, v_0)$ is the explicit Gaussian
$$
p(t, x, v ; x_0, v_0) \;=\; \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2\pi t^2}\;\exp\!\left[\;-\frac{3}{t^3}(x - x_0 - t v_0)^2 \;+\; \frac{3}{t^2}(x - x_0 - t v_0)(v - v_0) \;-\; \frac{1}{t}(v - v_0)^2\;\right]. \tag{28.3}
$$
(Kolmogorov 1934 *Math. Annalen* 108, equation 5; commonly cited as the *kinetic Fokker-Planck equation*.) This is the **G28 oracle** — the only closed-form hypoelliptic kernel used in the v3.1.0 release.

**Heisenberg group sub-Laplacian (constructive instance, NOT gated in v3.1, CITATION — Folland 1975 *Ark. Mat.* §2)**: on $\mathbb{H}^1 = \{(x, y, t) \in \mathbb{R}^3\}$ with the left-invariant fields $X_1 = \partial_x - \tfrac{y}{2} \partial_t$ and $X_2 = \partial_y + \tfrac{x}{2} \partial_t$, the sub-Laplacian $L = \tfrac{1}{2}(X_1^2 + X_2^2)$ is bracket-generating at step 2 ($[X_1, X_2] = \partial_t$). The heat kernel admits a closed form via complex-valued integrals (Beals-Gaveau-Greiner 1997 *Bull. Sci. Math.* 121); validation requires v4.0+ `SemiflowComplex` and is deferred. v3.1 ships `HeisenbergGroup<F>` as a **constructive instance** of the framework (compiles, runs, passes the step-2 checker) but does NOT gate convergence on it.

### §28.3 — Palindromic Strang-Hörmander decomposition (NORMATIVE library)

For a step-2 Carnot Hörmander generator $L = X_0 + \tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{k=1}^{M} X_k^2$ on $\mathbb{R}^D$, the v3.1 library ships the **palindromic Strang-Hörmander** Chernoff function:

$$
F(\tau) \;:=\; e^{\tau X_0 / 2} \circ \!\left(\prod_{k=1}^{M-1} e^{\tau X_k^2 / 2}\right) \circ e^{\tau X_M^2 / 2} \circ \!\left(\prod_{k=M-1}^{1} e^{\tau X_k^2 / 2}\right) \circ e^{\tau X_0 / 2}. \tag{28.4}
$$

Note the sandwich symmetry: $X_0$ on the outside (Strang half-steps), $X_M^2$ in the centre (full step), and the inner $X_k^2$ legs ($1 \le k \le M-1$) palindromic. For $M = 1$ (Kolmogorov), this collapses to the standard Strang split $F(\tau) = e^{\tau X_0 / 2} \circ e^{\tau X_1^2 / 2} \circ e^{\tau X_0 / 2}$.

**Per-leg exponentials**:
- $e^{\tau X_0 / 2}$ is a **drift** exponential — the flow along the integral curves of $X_0$ for time $\tau/2$. For closed-form Carnot backends, the flow is linear (Kolmogorov: $(x, v) \mapsto (x + (\tau/2) v, v)$; Heisenberg: $X_0 = 0$, identity).
- $e^{\tau X_k^2 / 2}$ is a **diffusive** exponential — the 1D heat semigroup along the integral curves of $X_k$. For closed-form Carnot backends, this admits the standard 1D heat-kernel convolution along $X_k$ flow lines (Kolmogorov: $(x, v) \mapsto$ Gaussian convolution in $v$; Heisenberg: structured 1D heat along the $X_k$ horizontal direction).

### §28.4 — Reference backends: closed-form Carnot groups (NORMATIVE library)

The v3.1 reference impls (all satisfy Definition 28.2 at step 2):

- **`KolmogorovPhaseSpace<F>` impl `VectorField<F, 2>` (math §28.4.A)**: $X_0 = v \cdot \partial_x$ (drift in $x$ along $v$), $X_1 = \partial_v$ (diffusion in $v$). The single bracket $[X_1, X_0] = \partial_x$ supplies the missing direction; step-2 verified at construction. Closed-form drift: $e^{\tau X_0}(x, v) = (x + \tau v, v)$ (exact, linear). Closed-form diffusion: $e^{\tau X_1^2 / 2} u(x, v) = (2\pi\tau)^{-1/2} \int e^{-(v - v')^2 / (2\tau)} u(x, v')\,dv'$ (1D heat kernel in $v$, $x$ frozen). The product formula $(F(\tau/n))^n$ converges to (28.3) at order 2 on $f \in D(L^2)$ (Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 with K=2).

- **`HeisenbergGroup<F>` impl `VectorField<F, 3>` (math §28.4.B)**: $X_1 = \partial_x - \tfrac{y}{2}\partial_t$, $X_2 = \partial_y + \tfrac{x}{2}\partial_t$, $X_0 = 0$ (no explicit drift). The bracket $[X_1, X_2] = \partial_t$ supplies the missing direction; step-2 verified. Closed-form per-leg diffusions: per-axis 1D heat kernels along the *horizontal* direction with the *vertical* coupling encoded by the $y/2$ and $x/2$ shifts (Folland 1975 §2.3). The palindromic Strang composition (28.4) is well-defined; the K=2 tangency on $f \in D(L^2)$ holds by the Galkin-Remizov 2025 framework. NOT GATED in v3.1: validation requires the explicit Heisenberg heat kernel which involves complex-valued integrals (Beals-Gaveau-Greiner 1997) — defer to v4.0+ when SemiflowComplex is available.

- **User-defined `VectorField<F, D>` backends** (open extensibility): compile via the `VectorField<F, D>` trait + `HypoellipticChernoff::new` constructor. The step-checker at construction verifies the bracket-generating condition at the grid centre via SVD on the bracket-evaluated matrix. **Step-2 only is GATED in v3.1.0**; user-defined step-3 (Engel group, free nilpotent step-3) backends FAIL the construction check and return `DomainViolation`. Step ≥ 3 user-defined backends defer to v3.2+ Tier C.

**§28 AMENDMENT (v4.x — ADR-0087 Heisenberg backend)**

The v3.1 deferral of the Heisenberg gate (§28.4.B above + §28.7 + §28.8) was based on the **misconception** that the Heisenberg sub-Laplacian heat kernel necessarily requires complex-valued arithmetic. This amendment supersedes that deferral: a *pure-real* closed-form integral representation is available and gives a `no_std + libm`-compatible oracle, evaluated to ≤ 10⁻¹⁰ accuracy by 32-pt Gauss-Legendre quadrature on a truncated symmetric interval. The full deferral rationale (§28.7 third bullet; §28.4.B last sentence) is retained in this document for historical traceability; the operative spec is replaced by the following.

**Gaveau-Hulanicki integral form (CITATION — Beals-Gaveau-Greiner 1997 *Bull. Sci. Math.* 121 §3, equation 3.1; original derivations Hulanicki ~1976 *Studia Math.* + Gaveau 1977 *Acta Math.* 139:95-153)**: on $\mathbb{H}^1 = \{(x, y, t) \in \mathbb{R}^3\}$ with coordinates $(x, y, t)$ and the sub-Laplacian $L = \tfrac{1}{2}(X_1^2 + X_2^2)$ generated by the left-invariant fields $X_1 = \partial_x - \tfrac{y}{2}\partial_t$, $X_2 = \partial_y + \tfrac{x}{2}\partial_t$, the heat kernel of $\partial_h u = L u$ at time $h > 0$ admits the explicit integral representation

$$
p_h(x, y, t) \;=\; \frac{1}{16\pi^2 h^2} \int_{-\infty}^{\infty} \frac{\lambda}{\sinh(\lambda h)} \exp\!\left(-\,\frac{r^2 \lambda \coth(\lambda h)}{4 h}\right) \cos\!\left(\frac{\lambda t}{h}\right) d\lambda,
\qquad r^2 := x^2 + y^2.
$$

The kernel is the *real part* of the canonical Hulanicki-form Fourier integral $\int (\lambda/\sinh \lambda h) \exp(-r^2 \lambda \coth(\lambda h)/(4h)) e^{i\lambda t/h} d\lambda$; the imaginary part vanishes by even-odd symmetry $\lambda \mapsto -\lambda$. **No complex arithmetic is required**; the integrand uses only $\sinh$, $\cosh$, $\exp$, $\cos$ (all available in `libm`). For the on-diagonal case $t = 0$ the $\cos$ factor reduces to unity and the kernel is the standard real positive density.

**Quadrature scheme (NORMATIVE library — ADR-0087)**: the integrand decays super-exponentially since $\lambda/\sinh(\lambda h) \sim 2\lambda e^{-|\lambda| h}$ as $|\lambda| h \to \infty$ and the Gaussian factor $\exp(-r^2 \lambda \coth(\lambda h)/(4h))$ is non-increasing on the tails. Truncating to the symmetric interval $[-\Lambda, +\Lambda]$ with $\Lambda := 25/h$ leaves a tail error bounded by $O(e^{-\Lambda h}) = O(e^{-25}) \approx 1.4 \times 10^{-11}$. On $[-\Lambda, +\Lambda]$, the integral is evaluated by **32-point Gauss-Legendre quadrature** using a pre-computed `f64` nodes/weights table — mirror of the existing v2.7 `resolvent_quad.rs` pattern (Cohort N/A; 75-LoC quadrature-tables module, ADR-0069). The composite accuracy target is $\le 10^{-10}$ uniform over the spatial probe set used by the gate.

**Convergence rate (NORMATIVE library — ADR-0087)**: on the Heisenberg backend `HeisenbergGroup<F>`, the palindromic Strang-Hörmander composition (§28.3 equation 28.4) attains order $2$ on $f \in D(L^2)$ by the Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 with $K = 2$ — the proof is identical to the Kolmogorov case (§28.5 G28) once the per-leg horizontal shifts $\exp(\tau X_k^2 / 2)$ are evaluated via the Gaveau-Hulanicki oracle. The acceptance gate `G_HORM_HEISENBERG` (§28.5 amendment) is the OLS slope of $\|F^n(f_0) - u_\mathrm{ref}\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ on a 3D Gaussian initial datum on $\mathbb{H}^1$, with floor $\le -1.95$ (mirror G28 margin convention). The sympy gate `T_HORM_HEISENBERG` adds four sub-checks: (i) PDE residual $\partial_h p - L p$ vanishes symbolically on a small spatial probe set; (ii) real-valuedness $\Im(p_h) = 0$ verified by closed-form $\lambda \mapsto -\lambda$ symmetry; (iii) normalization $\int p_h \,dx\,dy\,dt = 1$; (iv) step-2 Lie-bracket identity $[X_1, X_2] = \partial_t$ via `lie_bracket_kit.py`.

**§28 AMENDMENT 2 (v4.x — formula transcription correction; SUPERSEDES AMENDMENT 1 formula above)**

The formula given in AMENDMENT 1 above (`p_h = (1/(16π²h²)) · ∫ (λ/sinh(λh)) exp(−r²λcoth(λh)/(4h)) cos(λt/h) dλ`) is mathematically WRONG — it contains multiple transcription errors (spurious `1/h` factors in the exponent and `cos` argument, a factor-of-2 prefactor mistake, and incorrect operator-prefactor handling). The sympy gate `T_HORM_HEISENBERG.pde_residual` detected this: `|∂_h p − Lp| ≈ 1.9 × 10⁴` at the first probe `(h=0.1, x=y=t=0)` — kernel itself off by ~100× scale; see `.dev-docs/research/heisenberg-formula-diagnostic.md` for the full bug analysis and source-comparison table. The AMENDMENT 1 formula was inherited verbatim from `verdict-heisenberg.md` Q2.A, which itself was a researcher synthesis that did not cite a verbatim primary-source equation number. AMENDMENT 1 formula above is LOGICALLY DEPRECATED (retained verbatim for historical record); the canonical formula for the math.md operator-prefactor convention $L = \tfrac{1}{2}(X_1^2 + X_2^2)$ is:

$$
\boxed{
p_h(x, y, t) \;=\; \frac{1}{(2\pi)^2} \int_{-\infty}^{\infty} \frac{\lambda}{\sinh(\lambda h / 2)} \,
\exp\!\Big(-\,\tfrac{\lambda}{4}\,\coth(\lambda h / 2)\,(x^2 + y^2)\Big)\, \cos(\lambda t)\, d\lambda
}
$$

for $\partial_h u = L u = \tfrac{1}{2}(X_1^2 + X_2^2)\,u$ on $\mathbb{H}^1$ with the math.md convention $X_1 = \partial_x - \tfrac{y}{2}\partial_t$, $X_2 = \partial_y + \tfrac{x}{2}\partial_t$, $[X_1, X_2] = \partial_t$ (step-2 Carnot).

**Derivation chain**: The Krötz-Thangavelu-Xu 2005 arxiv math/0401243 form (eq 4.1.2 for the asymmetric algebra) gives the heat kernel for $L_{\text{full}} = X^2 + Y^2$ (no $\tfrac{1}{2}$ prefactor) as

$$
p_h^{L_{\text{full}}}(x, y, t) \;=\; \frac{1}{(2\pi)^2} \int_{-\infty}^{\infty} \frac{\lambda}{\sinh(\lambda h)} \exp\!\Big(-\tfrac{\lambda}{4}\coth(\lambda h)(x^2+y^2)\Big) \cos(\lambda t)\, d\lambda
$$

(verified by analytical computation: $p_h^{L_{\text{full}}}(0,0,0) = 1/(8h^2)$, and the heat equation $\partial_h p = (X^2+Y^2)\,p$ holds at all probe points to 4-digit accuracy under mpmath quadrature). For the math.md operator $L = \tfrac{1}{2}L_{\text{full}}$, we have $e^{hL} = e^{(h/2)L_{\text{full}}}$, so $p_h^L(x) = p_{h/2}^{L_{\text{full}}}(x)$. Substituting $h \to h/2$ in the $L_{\text{full}}$ formula gives the boxed expression. Verified: $p_h^L(0,0,0) = 1/(2h^2)$ and $\partial_h p = \tfrac{1}{2}(X^2+Y^2)\,p$ holds at all 6 probe points $(0,0,0), (0.5,0.5,0), (0.5,0.5,0.5)$ for $h \in \{0.1, 0.5\}$ to 4-digit accuracy under mpmath adaptive quadrature.

**Primary citation**: Beals, R. and Greiner, P.C. *Calculus on Heisenberg Manifolds*, Annals of Math Studies **119**, Princeton University Press, 1988, Theorem 5.18 (reproduces Hulanicki 1976 *Studia Math.* 56:165-173 explicit form for the symmetric convention; the operator-prefactor handling is standard for canonical-Hulanicki vs canonical-KTX formulations). Cross-checks: Krötz-Thangavelu-Xu 2005 arxiv math/0401243 equation (4.1.2) for the asymmetric algebra $L_{\text{full}} = X^2+Y^2$ kernel; Boggess-Raich 2007 arxiv 0711.4117 Corollary 1.4 for the asymmetric $L_γ = -\tfrac{1}{4} \Sigma(X^2+Y^2)$ convention (relates to math.md via factor-of-2 in operator rescaling). The boxed formula here is the operator-rescaled form ready for direct use with math.md's $L = \tfrac{1}{2}(X^2+Y^2)$.

**Quadrature scheme**: For the Rust engineer Wave implementation, use 32-pt Gauss-Legendre on $[-\Lambda, +\Lambda]$ with **$\Lambda := 16/h$** (NOT $25/h$ as in AMENDMENT 1, NOT $32/h$ either: numerical sweep shows $\Lambda = 16/h$ is optimal — at $\Lambda = 8/h$ on-diagonal accuracy is 4-digit; at $\Lambda = 16/h$ off-diagonal accuracy stays 4-digit and on-diagonal is 4-digit; at $\Lambda \ge 32/h$ off-diagonal under-samples the cos($\lambda t$) oscillation, dropping to 2-digit accuracy). For SYMPY-ORACLE reference quality (T_HORM_HEISENBERG), use mpmath adaptive `quad` (NOT 32-pt GL) to eliminate quadrature uncertainty as a confounder; the Rust impl's 32-pt GL is then validated against the mpmath oracle. Tail bound at $\Lambda h / 2 = 8$ is $O(e^{-16}) \approx 1.1 \times 10^{-7}$ (good); off-diagonal cos($\lambda t$) oscillation imposes an UPPER limit on $\Lambda$ that 32-pt GL can resolve — exceeding $\Lambda \approx 16/h$ at $h = 0.1, t = 0.5$ (giving $\lambda t$ range of 80) causes systematic under-sampling. Removable-singularity guard at $\lambda = 0$: $\lambda/\sinh(\lambda h / 2) \to 2/h$ and $(\lambda/4) \cdot \coth(\lambda h / 2) \to 1/(2h)$, so the integrand at $\lambda = 0$ has the closed limit $(2/h) \cdot \exp(-r^2/(2h)) \cdot 1$.

**Re-execution requirement (NORMATIVE — engineer Wave 2)**: `scripts/verify_hormander_heisenberg.py` MUST be updated to use this corrected formula and re-run; `T_HORM_HEISENBERG PASS` is the precondition for engineer-side Rust impl re-introduction. The pipeline ordering "sympy gate before engineer code" is hereby promoted from implicit-best-practice to NORMATIVE for all closed-form-kernel ADRs (§28 sets the precedent).

### §28.5 — Acceptance gates (G28 + G29 + T_HORM — NORMATIVE)

- **G28 (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0077): Kolmogorov-kernel slope ≤ −1.95 on step-2 Carnot.** Setup:
  ```rust
  // d=2 Kolmogorov phase space (x, v) on [-5, 5]^2 with reflecting BCs
  let grid = GridND::<f64, 2>::new([-5.0, -5.0], [5.0, 5.0], [n, n])?;
  let x0 = Box::new(KolmogorovPhaseSpace::<f64>::x0_drift());      // X_0 = v · ∂_x
  let x_diff: [Box<dyn VectorField<f64, 2>>; 1] = [
      Box::new(KolmogorovPhaseSpace::<f64>::x1_diffusion()),       // X_1 = ∂_v
  ];
  let kernel = HypoellipticChernoff::<f64, 2, 1>::new(x0, x_diff, grid.clone())?;
  ```
  Initial datum: $f_0(x, v) = \exp(-\tfrac{1}{2}(x^2 + v^2))$ (2D Gaussian).
  Horizon: $T = 0.5$.

  Reference solution: closed-form Kolmogorov fundamental-solution convolution per (28.3) — analytically evaluated at the final time $T$ for $f_0$ via the 2D Gaussian-Gaussian convolution identity (the Gaussian initial datum convolves with the Kolmogorov Gaussian to a closed-form Gaussian whose covariance is $\text{Cov}_{f_0} + \text{Cov}_{Kolm,T}$). Sympy script `verify_hormander_kolmogorov.py` writes the reference at f64 precision (T_HORM produces the reference table; the same script ships).

  Sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ at fixed $T = 0.5$ (so $\tau = T / n$). Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\|F^n(f_0) - u_{\mathrm{ref}}\|_\infty$ vs $1/n$ MUST be $\le -1.95$. (Asymptotic slope per Theorem 28.1 + Galkin-Remizov 2025 IJM K=2 is $-2.0$; the $-1.95$ floor has 2.5% margin and is the standard precedent for v3.x order-2 gates — mirror G_zeta4 / G27.) **Restricted to step-2 Carnot in v3.1.**

  Test file: `tests/hormander_kolmogorov_slope.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v3.1 release.

- **G29 (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0077): Mass conservation $\le 10^{-10}$ across G28 sweep.** Same setup as G28. At every $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$, verify $|\int p^{(n)}(T, x, v)\,dx\,dv - 1| \le 10^{-10}$ (using trapezoidal-rule integration on the 2D grid). The Kolmogorov heat semigroup is **sub-Markov** (mass-preserving for $f_0$ normalised to unit mass); G29 verifies that the Chernoff approximation `HypoellipticChernoff` preserves this property at every step. Failure indicates a structural bug in the palindromic Strang decomposition (typically a coefficient error in (28.4)).

  Test file: same as G28 (`tests/hormander_kolmogorov_slope.rs` — combined slope + mass gate). Failure BLOCKS v3.1 release.

- **T_HORM (NORMATIVE sympy — ADR-0077): Kolmogorov 1934 fundamental solution symbolic verification.** Sympy verification of (28.3) — 4 sub-checks (all mandatory):
  1. **(T_HORM.pde_residual)** Substitute the explicit Gaussian (28.3) into the Kolmogorov PDE $\partial_t p = v \partial_x p + \tfrac{1}{2} \partial_v^2 p$ symbolically. Verify the residual is **literally zero** (use `sympy.simplify` + `sympy.expand`). This validates the closed-form kernel for the v3.1 G28 oracle.
  2. **(T_HORM.initial_condition)** Verify $\lim_{t \to 0^+} p(t, x, v; x_0, v_0) = \delta(x - x_0)\delta(v - v_0)$ in the distributional sense, by computing the first moment $\int x \cdot p\,dx\,dv$ symbolically and verifying it equals $x_0 + t v_0$ at $t \to 0^+$.
  3. **(T_HORM.first_moment)** Verify the first moment of $p$ in $x$: $\int x \cdot p(t, x, v; x_0, v_0)\,dx\,dv = x_0 + t v_0$ symbolically (the Kolmogorov mean transport equation). This is the *constructive* test for the v3.1 G28 reference solution.
  4. **(T_HORM.mass)** Verify $\int p(t, x, v; x_0, v_0)\,dx\,dv = 1$ symbolically for all $t > 0$ — the foundation of G29's numerical mass-conservation gate.

  Script: `scripts/verify_hormander_kolmogorov.py` (new file, ~250 LoC, ships in v3.1 Wave A engineer). MUST print exactly `T_HORM PASS` on success (all 4 sub-checks pass) or `T_HORM FAIL: <reason>` on failure (any sub-check fails). Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_v2_*.py` + `verify_manifold_torus.py` + `verify_zeta4_correction.py` + the v3.1 sibling `verify_quantum_graph_kirchhoff.py`. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; safe for CI without `slow-tests`. Failure BLOCKS v3.1 release.

### §28.6 — `VectorField<F, D>` trait + `HypoellipticChernoff<F, D, M>` (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub trait VectorField<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize> {
    /// Writes the vector-field value v_x = X(x) into out. out.len() == D.
    /// Returns DomainViolation on any NaN/Inf in x or out, or shape mismatch.
    fn evaluate(&self, x: &[F; D], out: &mut [F; D]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError>;

    /// Optional: writes the Lie bracket [self, other](x) into out via the
    /// directional-derivative formula
    ///   [X, Y](x) = (dY|_x) · X(x) - (dX|_x) · Y(x).
    /// Default impl uses central-difference Jacobians at f64 precision; backends
    /// with closed-form Jacobians (closed-form Carnot fields) override for
    /// sympy-traceable accuracy. Used by the step-checker at construction time.
    fn bracket_with(
        &self,
        other: &dyn VectorField<F, D>,
        x: &[F; D],
        out: &mut [F; D],
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // Default: central-difference Jacobians with h = F::EPSILON^(1/3).
        // Backends MAY override for closed-form accuracy.
        todo!("default impl per math §28.6")
    }
}

pub struct HypoellipticChernoff<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize, const M: usize> {
    x0_drift: Box<dyn VectorField<F, D>>,
    x_diff: [Box<dyn VectorField<F, D>>; M],
    grid: GridND<F, D>,
    step_checker_result: StepCheckerResult,    // cached at construction; step ∈ {1, 2}; step ≥ 3 = DomainViolation
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize, const M: usize> HypoellipticChernoff<F, D, M> {
    pub fn new(
        x0_drift: Box<dyn VectorField<F, D>>,
        x_diff: [Box<dyn VectorField<F, D>>; M],
        grid: GridND<F, D>,
    ) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize, const M: usize> ChernoffFunction<F>
    for HypoellipticChernoff<F, D, M>
{
    type S = GridFnND<F, D>;

    fn apply_into(
        &self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // Per math §28.3 equation (28.4) — palindromic Strang-Hörmander.
        // 1. apply_x0_drift(τ/2, src, dst1, scratch)
        // 2. for k in 1..M: apply_xk_squared(τ, k, dst1, dst1, scratch)
        // 3. apply_xk_squared(τ, M, dst1, dst1, scratch)               // middle full step
        // 4. for k in (1..M).rev(): apply_xk_squared(τ, k, dst1, dst1, scratch)
        // 5. apply_x0_drift(τ/2, dst1, dst, scratch)
        todo!()
    }

    fn order(&self) -> u32 { 2 }              // per Theorem 28.1 + Galkin-Remizov K=2

    fn growth(&self) -> Growth<F> {           // v3.0 typed return per ADR-0074
        Growth { multiplier: F::one(), omega: F::zero() }
    }
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat, const D: usize, const M: usize> ApproximationSubspace<2, F>
    for HypoellipticChernoff<F, D, M>
{
    fn in_subspace(&self, f: &Self::S) -> bool {
        // ≥ 5^D grid points per axis; backend-specific extra checks
        todo!()
    }
    fn jet(&self, f: &Self::S, out: &mut [Self::S]) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // out: [f, L f, L² f]; L = X_0 + (1/2) Σ X_k²
        // 2 iterations of the discretised Hörmander operator
        todo!()
    }
}
```

### §28.bis — Engel step-3 filiform Carnot Chernoff approximation (v4.5+, ADR-0095, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

**Scope amendment to §28.7 step-2 restriction.** The v3.1 deferral of step ≥ 3 Carnot backends (§28.7 first bullet) was based on the assumption that closed-form heat-kernel oracles are required for the gate. This assumption is **lifted** for the Engel case via **self-convergence** gating (mirror of v2.2 `G_NS2D_aniso` pattern; no closed-form oracle needed). Bonfiglioli-Lanconelli-Uguzzoni 2007 (the canonical 812-pp. Springer reference) confirms that **no closed-form heat kernel exists for the Engel group in this canonical reference** — the Folland-Kaplan formula (Theorem 18.3.1) is restricted to H-type groups and Engel is NOT H-type. Self-convergence is therefore not just *one* path but the *only viable* path for Engel.

#### §28.bis.1 — Engel filiform N=4 step-3 Carnot group (CITATION — Bonfiglioli 2007 §4.3.6, Prop. 4.3.8 + Theorem 4.3.6/Bratzlavsky 1974)

The **Engel group** $E$ is the unique (up to isomorphism) non-trivial filiform Carnot group of dimension $N = 4$; equivalently, the smallest non-trivial step-3 Carnot group (Bonfiglioli Prop. 4.3.8 + Remark 4.3.9). Coordinates $(x_1, x_2, x_3, x_4) \in \mathbb{R}^4$. Stratification $g = g_1 \oplus g_2 \oplus g_3$ with $\dim g_1 = 2$, $\dim g_2 = \dim g_3 = 1$.

**Left-invariant fields (Bratzlavsky basis per Theorem 4.3.6)**:
$$
X_1 = \partial_{x_1}, \qquad X_2 = \partial_{x_2} + x_1 \partial_{x_3} + \tfrac{x_1^2}{2} \partial_{x_4}, \tag{28.bis.1}
$$
$$
X_3 := [X_1, X_2] = \partial_{x_3} + x_1 \partial_{x_4}, \qquad X_4 := [X_1, X_3] = \partial_{x_4}. \tag{28.bis.2}
$$

**Filiform termination relations** (verified by `T_HORM_ENGEL_BRACKETS` sympy gate):
$$
[X_2, X_3] = 0, \qquad [X_i, X_4] = 0 \quad \text{for all } i \in \{1, 2, 3\}. \tag{28.bis.3}
$$

The bracket-generating depth is **exactly 3** (Hörmander step 3): $\dim \mathrm{span}\{X_1, X_2\}|_0 = 2$, $\dim \mathrm{span}\{X_1, X_2, X_3\}|_0 = 3$, $\dim \mathrm{span}\{X_1, X_2, X_3, X_4\}|_0 = 4 = D$.

**Sub-Laplacian**: $L_E := X_1^2 + X_2^2$ on $\mathbb{R}^4$. Hypoelliptic by Hörmander Theorem 1.1 (§28.2 Theorem 28.1) at step 3.

#### §28.bis.2 — Palindromic Strang-Hörmander on Engel (NORMATIVE library)

The Chernoff function $F_E(\tau)$ is the palindromic Strang-Hörmander composition (math.md §28.3 eq 28.4) with $M = 2$ horizontal fields and $X_0 = 0$:
$$
F_E(\tau) \;:=\; e^{\tau X_1^2 / 4} \;\circ\; e^{\tau X_2^2 / 2} \;\circ\; e^{\tau X_1^2 / 4}. \tag{28.bis.4}
$$

**Per-leg exponentials** (NORMATIVE library — Engineer Wave §"AC4"):

- $e^{\sigma X_1^2}$ is the 1D heat semigroup along the constant integral curves of $X_1 = \partial_{x_1}$ — Gaussian convolution in $x_1$, other coordinates frozen.
- $e^{\sigma X_2^2}$ is the 1D heat semigroup along the polynomial integral curves of $X_2 = \partial_{x_2} + x_1 \partial_{x_3} + (x_1^2/2) \partial_{x_4}$. The integral curve through $(x_1, x_2, x_3, x_4)$ at parameter $s$ is (verified by ODE integration of $X_2$ component-wise: $\dot x_1 = 0$, $\dot x_2 = 1$, $\dot x_3 = x_1$, $\dot x_4 = x_1^2 / 2$, all coefficients evaluated at the *starting* point $x_1$ which is preserved along the flow):
$$
\Phi_s^{X_2}(x_1, x_2, x_3, x_4) \;=\; (x_1,\, x_2 + s,\, x_3 + s\, x_1,\, x_4 + s\, x_1^2 / 2). \tag{28.bis.5}
$$
The Gaussian convolution weight on $s$ is $G_\sigma(s) = (4\pi\sigma)^{-1/2} \exp(-s^2/(4\sigma))$; quadrature is 32-pt Gauss-Hermite (mirror v3.x Heisenberg `heisenberg_diffuse_x2` pattern; nodes/weights re-used verbatim). **No special functions beyond `exp` and `sqrt`; pure `no_std + libm`.**

**Theorem 28.bis (conditional order-2 tangency on Engel)**: on $f \in D(L_E^2)$, the composition $(F_E(\tau/n))^n$ converges to $e^{\tau L_E} f$ at rate $O(1/n^2)$ in the strong operator topology, **provided** the Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 K=2 tangency framework extends to step-3 Carnot generators. The framework's hypothesis is a Taylor remainder bound on $S(t)f - \sum_{k=0}^{K-1} t^k L^k f / k!$, which is operator-algebraic and *does not* depend on the step of the underlying Carnot group; extension is **plausible** but **unproven**. The self-convergence gate `G_HORM_ENGEL` (§28.bis.4 below) provides the empirical witness.

#### §28.bis.3 — Sympy verification `T_HORM_ENGEL_BRACKETS` (NORMATIVE — architect-side PASS precondition)

Per the §28 AMENDMENT 2 NORMATIVE re-execution requirement, the architect MUST run `scripts/verify_engel_brackets.py` and confirm PASS BEFORE delegating Engineer Wave. The script verifies 5 sub-checks on the Bonfiglioli-Lanconelli-Uguzzoni 2007 §4.3.6 Bratzlavsky-basis formulas (28.bis.1) + (28.bis.2):

1. $[X_1, X_2] = X_3 = \partial_{x_3} + x_1 \cdot \partial_{x_4}$ symbolically.
2. $[X_1, X_3] = X_4 = \partial_{x_4}$ symbolically.
3. $[X_2, X_3] = 0$ symbolically.
4. Filiform termination: $[X_i, X_4] = 0$ for $i \in \{1, 2, 3\}$ ($X_4$ in centre).
5. Hörmander rank 4: $\dim \mathrm{span}\{X_1, X_2, X_3, X_4\}|_{x=0} = 4$.

Plus diagnostic verification that step-2 brackets alone have rank 3 (strictly < 4), confirming Engel is genuinely step-3 and not a degenerate step-2 in disguise. **PASS at architect-side 2026-05-29** (ADR-0095 acceptance); engineer Wave reuses script in CI sweep.

#### §28.bis.4 — `G_HORM_ENGEL` self-convergence gate (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0095)

**No closed-form oracle exists** for the Engel heat kernel (Bonfiglioli 2007 §5.3 + §18.3-§18.5; Folland 1975 hypoellipticity gives existence only). Validation uses the **probe-vs-2N-1 self-convergence** pattern committed at v2.2 in `G_NS2D_aniso` (mirror; see `[[project-g4-ns2d-aniso-self-convergence]]`).

Setup:
```rust
// d=4 Engel coordinates (x1, x2, x3, x4) on [-3, 3]^4, 32 nodes per axis
let grid = Grid4D::<f64>::new([-3.0; 4], [3.0; 4], [32; 4])?;
let kernel = HypoellipticChernoff::<f64, 4, 2>::new_engel()?;
// IC: 4D Gaussian f₀(x) = exp(-||x||²/2)
let f0 = GridFn4D::from_fn(grid, |x1, x2, x3, x4| {
    (-(x1*x1 + x2*x2 + x3*x3 + x4*x4) * 0.5).exp()
});
```
Horizon $T = 0.5$. Sweep $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$. For each $n$:
$$
u_n := F_E(T/n)^n f_0, \qquad u_{2n} := F_E(T/(2n))^{2n} f_0, \qquad \mathrm{err}_n := \|u_n - u_{2n}\|_\infty. \tag{28.bis.6}
$$

Empirical $\log$-$\log$ OLS slope of $\mathrm{err}_n$ vs $n$ MUST be $\le -1.95$ (mirror G28 + G_HORM_HEISENBERG margin convention; 2.5% margin vs theoretical $-2.0$ from Theorem 28.bis). Failure interpretation:

- **Slope $\le -1.95$**: Theorem 28.bis hypothesis empirically confirmed → ship as v4.5+ feature; Festschrift §3 problem empirically advanced.
- **Slope $\in (-1.95, -1.0)$**: partial confirmation → ship as `experimental`; ADR amendment downgrading G_HORM_ENGEL gate to ADVISORY.
- **Slope $> -1.0$ or flat**: hypothesis refuted → Outcome B fallback per ADR-0095 §"Consequences"; reaffirm Item 3 STILL_OPEN; defer Rothschild-Stein lifting path to v5.x.

Test file: `crates/semiflow-core/tests/hormander_engel_slope.rs` (Engineer Wave; feature `slow-tests`; mirror `hormander_heisenberg_slope.rs` verbatim). Memory: 32⁴ × 8 B ≈ 8 MB per state. Wallclock estimate: ~30 s per probe on i7-12700K (4 probes × 2 grids ≈ 4 min; well under existing test-flagship budget).

#### §28.bis.5 — Limitations and future research

- **Order-2 only.** Order ≥ 3 on Engel inherits the Festschrift §3 open problem (math.md §28.7 second bullet); not addressed by ADR-0095.
- **Single Engel backend.** Free nilpotent step-3 backends (5+ dimensional) deferred to v5.x; same algorithm via `VectorField<F, D>` with $D \ge 5$.
- **Theorem 28.bis is conditional.** The K=2 tangency extension to step-3 Carnot is plausible (operator-algebraic hypothesis is step-agnostic) but unproven. Theoretical resolution deferred to v4.6+ math review.
- **Rothschild-Stein lifting (Bonfiglioli Ch. 17)** as v5.x alternative validation path: lift Engel to a free Carnot group of higher dimension where the kernel might be more tractable, run the approximation there, project back. Documented for future reference; not currently a v4.5 candidate.
- **Galkin-Remizov 2023 super-order phenomenon**: empirically unexplained $\alpha_S \approx -3.1$ for 1D heat with $u_0 = \exp(-x^4)$ initial datum. If generalises to Engel with exponential-decay 4D initial data, G_HORM_ENGEL slope may *exceed* $-2.0$ in measurable regime. Engineer Wave records observed slope verbatim; architect amends ADR if super-order phenomenon manifests.

#### §28.bis.7 — Step-4 (filiform N=5) palindrome tangency: F4 spike proof sketch (v8.0.0, ADR-0136)

**Scope.** This subsection records the math-prerequisite finding of the v8.0.0 F4 spike (the
"step-k Carnot closure via recursive palindrome-of-palindromes" direction, ADR-0136). It is a
NARROW result: it proves the order-2 gate for a concrete step-4 group and, in doing so,
delimits exactly what the recursive-nesting hypothesis does and does **not** buy. The genuine
Festschrift §3 open problem (a constructive order ≥ 3 hypoelliptic approximant) remains OPEN
and is **not** closed here. Symbolic witness: `scripts/carnot_step4_kit.py` (`T_CARNOT_STEP4`,
PASS at architect time 2026-06-07).

**Step-4 test group (filiform N=5).** Coordinates $(x_1,\dots,x_5)\in\mathbb{R}^5$;
stratification $g = g_1\oplus g_2\oplus g_3\oplus g_4$ with $\dim = (2,1,1,1)$. Bratzlavsky
filiform basis (Bonfiglioli 2007 §4.3.6, the N=5 sibling of the Engel N=4 group of §28.bis.1):
$$
X_1 = \partial_{x_1},\quad
X_2 = \partial_{x_2} + x_1\partial_{x_3} + \tfrac{x_1^2}{2}\partial_{x_4} + \tfrac{x_1^3}{6}\partial_{x_5},
\tag{28.bis.7a}
$$
$$
X_3 := [X_1,X_2] = \partial_{x_3} + x_1\partial_{x_4} + \tfrac{x_1^2}{2}\partial_{x_5},\quad
X_4 := [X_1,X_3] = \partial_{x_4} + x_1\partial_{x_5},\quad
X_5 := [X_1,X_4] = \partial_{x_5}.
\tag{28.bis.7b}
$$
All other brackets vanish (filiform termination). Hörmander rank at the origin: $2,3,4,5$ at
bracket depths $0,1,2,3$ respectively — genuine step 4 (step-3 brackets alone have rank 4 < 5).
Sub-Laplacian $L_5 := X_1^2 + X_2^2$. (Verified by `T_CARNOT_STEP4` Witness B-1.)

**Lemma 28.bis.7 (palindromic Strang is order-2 tangent, step-independently).** Let $A,B$ be
any two (possibly non-commuting) operators and
$$
\Psi(\tau) := e^{(\tau/2)A}\,e^{\tau B}\,e^{(\tau/2)A}.
$$
Then in the free associative algebra on $\{A,B\}$,
$$
\log\Psi(\tau) = \tau(A+B) \;+\; 0\cdot\tau^2 \;+\; \tau^3\!\left(-\tfrac{1}{24}[A,[A,B]] + \tfrac{1}{12}[B,[B,A]]\right) + O(\tau^5).
\tag{28.bis.7c}
$$
The $\tau^2$ coefficient vanishes by the palindromic symmetry $\Psi(\tau)^{-1} = \Psi(-\tau)$
(the odd-function property of $\log\Psi$; Hairer–Lubich–Wanner 2006 §III.5, Theorem 5.1); the
$\tau^3$ coefficient is generically non-zero. Hence $(\Psi(\tau/n))^n \to e^{\tau(A+B)}$ at
**global order 2** by the Galkin–Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 K=2 tangency framework. *This
identity does not reference the Carnot step.* (Verified symbolically by `T_CARNOT_STEP4`
Witness A: $\tau^2$ coeff $\equiv 0$, $\tau^3$ coeff matches (28.bis.7c) exactly and is non-zero.)

**Corollary 28.bis.7 (order-2 on the step-4 group).** Taking $A=\tfrac12 X_1^2$, $B=\tfrac12 X_2^2$
(the leg generators of (28.bis.4), since the diffusive legs of §28.3 are $e^{\sigma X_k^2/2}$),
the flat horizontal palindromic Strang $F_5(\tau) = e^{\tau X_1^2/4}\circ e^{\tau X_2^2/2}\circ e^{\tau X_1^2/4}$
is order-2 tangent to $e^{\tau L_5/2}$ on the filiform step-4 group. **Crux measurement:** the
operator residual $F_5(\tau)f - e^{(\tau/2)L_5}f$, evaluated EXACTLY on a generic degree-5
polynomial jet, first disagrees at $\tau^3$ (e.g. residual $-\tfrac{5}{48}x_1x_3 - \tfrac{11}{48}x_4 - \tfrac{1}{24}$),
confirming global order **exactly 2** (slope $-2$). (`T_CARNOT_STEP4` Witness B-2.)

**On the "palindrome-of-palindromes" recursion (ADR-0136 hypothesis).** The induction-step
claim — that *nesting* one palindrome around an inner-level product is what extends the
construction to higher step while preserving the tangency order — is **not required for the
order-2 gate** and is therefore not the mechanism the gate validates. Lemma 28.bis.7 shows the
*flat, un-nested* horizontal Strang already achieves order 2 on a step-4 generator with no
recursion: the depth-$k$ brackets $X_3,X_4,X_5$ are never exponentiated as legs; they enter
only implicitly through the non-commutativity of the two horizontal flows $e^{\sigma X_1^2}$,
$e^{\sigma X_2^2}$, and the palindromic symmetry cancels their leading effect at $\tau^2$ for
*any* step. The Carnot step affects only **hypoellipticity** (whether $e^{\tau L}$ is smoothing,
via Hörmander's bracket condition) — not the **order** of the splitting approximation. One level
of palindrome nesting trivially preserves order 2 (it embeds an order-2 sub-product as a single
order-2 leg), but this is a statement about composition of order-2 methods, **not** a route to a
*higher* order, which is where the genuine difficulty lives.

**What remains OPEN (honest delimitation).** The Festschrift §3 open problem is a constructive
*order ≥ 3* hypoelliptic approximant. Reaching order ≥ 3 by splitting requires correction legs
along the bracket (commutator) directions — the regime in which "treat $[Y,Z]$ as an effective
field $W$" (ADR-0136) becomes load-bearing, exactly as in Suzuki–Yoshida higher-order splitting.
That construction's induction step (that adding bracket-direction legs raises the order without
leaving an irreducible residual at the next BCH depth) is **not closed** by this spike: Lemma
28.bis.7 stops at order 2. The $\tau^3$ coefficient (28.bis.7c) is the obstruction — it is
non-zero and is *not* cancelled by any single extra palindromic wrap of the existing two legs.
A genuine order-≥3 step-$k$ construction would have to introduce new legs that cancel
(28.bis.7c)'s nested commutators; whether the recursive palindrome-of-palindromes does this for
general $k$ is the unproven, open part. **Mirroring the G_zeta4 escalation precedent (math §27,
ADR-0075), the higher-order step-$k$ direction is escalated, not declared closed.**

**Consequence for the F4 gate (NARROW).** `G_CARNOT_STEP4` is declared RELEASE_BLOCKING **only**
for the order-2 flat-horizontal palindromic Strang on the filiform step-4 (N=5) group, with the
self-convergence slope gate $\le -1.95$ (mirror G28 / G_HORM_ENGEL margin convention). It is
**not** a witness for any recursive-nesting / higher-order closure of the general-$k$ problem.
The v8.0.0 "all-blocking F4" scope is correspondingly reduced to this provable family; the
general-$k$ and order-≥3 closure stays OPEN (ADR-0136 → NARROW per its stated fallback).

**Honesty note on prior super-slope.** The previously recorded Engel self-convergence slope of
$\approx -43.95$ ("super-exponential") is an **artifact** of an origin-centred Gaussian initial
datum, on which the $\tau^3$ residual nearly vanishes (the polynomial flow coefficients
$x_1,\,x_1^2/2,\,x_1^3/6$ are small near the origin). The spike reproduced this artifact with a
low-degree, near-symmetric test function (residual $\equiv 0$ through $\tau^4$) and then
dispelled it with a generic degree-5 jet (residual $\ne 0$ at $\tau^3$). The genuine order is
**2**, not super-order. Self-convergence gates on Carnot groups MUST use a generic
(non-origin-symmetric, sufficiently high-degree) probe; otherwise they over-report the order.

#### §28.bis.8 — Complex-time order-4 Carnot Chernoff via the complex triple-jump (v8.0.0, ADR-0136 Amendment 2, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

**Scope.** §28.bis.7 proved the *real-coefficient* horizontal palindromic Strang is order **2** on any
Carnot step, the obstruction being the non-zero $\tau^3$ commutator coefficient
$-\tfrac{1}{24}[A,[A,B]] + \tfrac{1}{12}[B,[B,A]]$ (eq. 28.bis.7c). This subsection records the v8.0.0 F4
**INVENTIVE** re-spike result: a *complex-coefficient* construction that **escapes the Sheng–Suzuki order
barrier** and reaches global order **4** on a genuine step-4 Carnot sub-Laplacian, with every substep
forward-in-time (bounded). Symbolic witness: `scripts/carnot_complex_order3_kit.py` (`T_CARNOT_CPLX3`, PASS
16/16 at architect time 2026-06-07). This is the operative STRONG-GO result of F4; the §28.bis.7 NARROW
order-2 statement is preserved as the real-coefficient baseline.

**The Sheng–Suzuki order barrier (the physical obstruction).** For a *real-coefficient* splitting
$\prod_j e^{c_j\tau A}e^{d_j\tau B}$ of order $\ge 3$, at least one coefficient is **negative** (Sheng 1989,
IMA J. Numer. Anal. 9; Goldman–Kaper 1996, SIAM J. Numer. Anal. 33). A negative substep evolves the
sub-Laplacian semigroup **backward in time**, $e^{-|c|\tau L}$, which is **unbounded** (the backward heat /
hypoelliptic flow is ill-posed). Hence order-2 is the naive ceiling for any bounded real splitting — exactly
the §28.bis.7 finding.

**The escape (complex time on an analytic semigroup).** The Carnot sub-Laplacian $L=X_1^2+X_2^2$ generates
an **analytic** (sectorial) semigroup (Hörmander hypoellipticity $\Rightarrow$ $e^{\tau L}$ is analytic), so
$e^{-c\tau L}$ is **bounded for every complex $c$ with $\Re c > 0$** (the value lies in the sector
$|\arg c| < \pi/2$). Complex coefficients with **positive real part** therefore supply order $\ge 3$ with
*bounded* (forward, sectorial) substeps — the Castella–Chartier–Descombes–Vilmart (BIT 49, 2009) /
Hansen–Ostermann (BIT 49, 2009) escape, here instantiated on a hypoelliptic generator.

**Construction 28.bis.8 (complex triple-jump).** Let $S(s)$ be the order-2 symmetric horizontal Strang map
$S(s) = e^{sX_1^2/4}\circ e^{sX_2^2/2}\circ e^{sX_1^2/4}$ of §28.bis.7 (the leg generators are
$\tfrac12 X_1^2,\tfrac12 X_2^2$). Define the **complex triple-jump**
$$
\Psi(\tau) \;:=\; S(\gamma\tau)\,\circ\,S\bigl((1-2\gamma)\tau\bigr)\,\circ\,S(\gamma\tau),
\tag{28.bis.8a}
$$
with $\gamma$ a root of the standard triple-jump cubic
$$
2\gamma^3 + (1-2\gamma)^3 = 0.
\tag{28.bis.8b}
$$
The three real roots-or-complex-roots are $\{\,1.3512072,\; 0.3243966 \mp 0.1345863\,i\,\}$. The **real**
root forces $1-2\gamma = -1.7024144 < 0$ (the Sheng–Suzuki backward step — rejected). The **complex
conjugate pair**
$$
\boxed{\;\gamma^\star = 0.32439640402017117 \,\mp\, 0.1345862724908067\,i,\qquad
1-2\gamma^\star = 0.35120719195965766 \,\pm\, 0.2691725449816134\,i\;}
\tag{28.bis.8c}
$$
has $\Re(\gamma^\star)=0.324 > 0$ **and** $\Re(1-2\gamma^\star)=0.351 > 0$ — **every sub-map runs forward in
(complex) time**, so every factor $e^{c\tau X_k^2}$ is a bounded sectorial-semigroup value.

**Lemma 28.bis.8 (order 4, step-independent).** In the free associative algebra on $\{A,B\}$, with
$A=\tfrac12 X_1^2$, $B=\tfrac12 X_2^2$, the complex triple-jump (28.bis.8a) at $\gamma=\gamma^\star$
satisfies
$$
\log\Psi(\tau) = \tau(A+B) + 0\cdot\tau^2 + 0\cdot\tau^3 + 0\cdot\tau^4 + O(\tau^5).
\tag{28.bis.8d}
$$
The $\tau^2$ coefficient vanishes by palindromic symmetry (each $S$ is symmetric and the scale sequence
$(\gamma,1-2\gamma,\gamma)$ is palindromic). The $\tau^3$ coefficient is proportional to the cubic
(28.bis.8b) for **both** independent commutator words $[A,[A,B]]$ and $[B,[B,A]]$, hence vanishes at
$\gamma^\star$. The $\tau^4$ coefficient vanishes **automatically**: a symmetric method of order 3 is order
4 by the even-order theorem ($\log\Psi(\tau)$ is an odd function of $\tau$ — Hairer–Lubich–Wanner 2006
§III.5). Therefore $(\Psi(\tau/n))^n \to e^{\tau(A+B)}$ at **global order 4** by the Galkin–Remizov 2025
*IJM* tangency framework (with its analytic-semigroup complex-time extension — CCDV 2009). *This identity
does not reference the Carnot step* (verified symbolically by `T_CARNOT_CPLX3` Witness A-3:
$\tau^2,\tau^3,\tau^4$ coefficients all $\equiv 0$ at $\gamma^\star$, the complex root admissible with
$\Re>0$ on both maps; the real root rejected for $\Re(1-2\gamma)<0$).

**Corollary 28.bis.8 (order 4 on the step-4 group).** On the filiform step-4 group (28.bis.7a/b), the
operator residual $\Psi(\tau)f - e^{(\tau/2)L_5}f$, evaluated EXACTLY on a **generic degree-10** non-origin
polynomial jet, first disagrees at $\tau^5$ (global order 4, slope $-4$), whereas the real flat Strang on
the *identical* jet first disagrees at $\tau^3$ (global order 2, slope $-2$). The degree-10 probe is
mandatory: $L=X_1^2+X_2^2$ is second-order, so $L^k$ lowers polynomial degree by 2 and a degree-5 jet makes
$L^3 f\equiv 0$, spuriously vanishing the residual past $\tau^3$ for *any* method (the ADR-0136 Amendment 1
honesty-note artifact). The real-Strang control reproducing order 2 on the same probe certifies the probe
is non-degenerate. (Verified by `T_CARNOT_CPLX3` Witness B.)

**Real-valued output.** For a real physical initial datum $f$, the order-4 real result is recovered as
$u(\tau)=\Re\bigl[\Psi_{\gamma^\star}(\tau)f\bigr]$: the two conjugate roots $\gamma^\star,\overline{\gamma^\star}$
give conjugate iterates, so taking $\Re(\cdot)$ after the full step is exactly their average and is
order-4-accurate and real. The intermediate state is complex-valued (a complex variance $c\sigma$ in each
Gaussian-convolution leg), which is why the kernel requires the complex substrate `SemiflowComplex` /
`GridFnND<C>` (math §30.2).

**Honest scope and conditionality.**
- The result is a **tangency-order** statement (local truncation order), proven symbolically. Strong-operator
  convergence at the global order-4 rate follows from the Galkin–Remizov tangency framework **provided** it
  admits complex-time substeps on analytic generators (the CCDV/Hansen–Ostermann setting); the library
  reproduces the *statement*, the proof of the complex-time case lives in the cited papers. Same conditional
  status as Theorem 28.bis (order-2 Engel); gated **empirically** by self-convergence `G_CARNOT_CPLX3`.
- $\Re(c)>0$ guarantees each factor is bounded; the operator-norm constant $M\ge 1$ of the sector is
  benign for sectorial $L$ (CCDV 2009 Thm 2.1) and is certified empirically by the slope gate.
- This **supersedes** the original ADR-0136 "palindrome-of-palindromes" mechanism (correctly NARROWed in
  Amendment 1: real nesting never beats order 2). The order-4 escape is the *complex* triple-jump — a
  different and stronger mechanism — not real nesting.

**Acceptance gate `G_CARNOT_CPLX3` (RELEASE_BLOCKING, ADR-0136 Amendment 2).** Self-convergence
probe-vs-2N on the filiform N=5 complex triple-jump, $T=0.5$, sweep $n\in\{8,16,32,64\}$, generic
non-origin high-degree IC, OLS slope $\le -3.80$ (order-4 with the G28 2.5%-margin convention vs theoretical
$-4$). Failure ladder: $\le -3.80$ PASS (order 4); $(-3.80,-2.85]$ ship `experimental` as order-3 (symmetry
bonus lost at discretisation — still beats the open problem); $> -2.85$ escalate. Sympy precondition
`T_CARNOT_CPLX3` PASS (architect-side 2026-06-07). Test file `tests/carnot_cplx3_slope.rs` (engineer Wave;
feature `slow-tests`; mirror `hormander_engel_slope.rs`).

### §28.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Step-2 Carnot only in v3.1.0; Engel step-3 added in v4.5+ via ADR-0095.** User-defined step-≥ 3 backends compile via `VectorField<F, D>` but FAIL the v3.1 step-2 SVD-rank checker. v4.5+ adds Engel as the **first** step-3 backend via the dedicated `HypoellipticChernoff::<f64, 4, 2>::new_engel()` constructor (ADR-0095; §28.bis); free nilpotent step-3 backends (D ≥ 5) deferred to v5.x. The Folland-Stein dilations + non-isotropic Hardy spaces needed for *general* step-3 theory remain substantial additional content; ADR-0095 sidesteps the closed-form-oracle requirement via self-convergence gating.
- **Order-2 only in v3.1.0; order-4 via complex time in v8.0.0.** Order ≥ 3 was the **Festschrift §3 open problem** in v3.1; it is **constructively achieved at order 4 in v8.0.0** via the complex triple-jump (§28.bis.8, ADR-0136 Amendment 2): complex-coefficient time-scales with positive real part escape the Sheng-Suzuki real-coefficient order barrier on the analytic Carnot semigroup. The v8.0 result is a *tangency-order* statement gated empirically by self-convergence (`G_CARNOT_CPLX3`); the strong-operator convergence theorem inherits the Galkin-Remizov tangency framework's complex-time/analytic-semigroup extension (CCDV 2009). Real-coefficient splittings remain capped at order 2 (the barrier is genuine and unescapable in ℝ).
- **Heisenberg gate deferred to v4.0+.** The Heisenberg sub-Laplacian fundamental solution involves complex-valued Bessel functions (Beals-Gaveau-Greiner 1997); validation requires v4.0+ `SemiflowComplex`. v3.1 ships `HeisenbergGroup<F>` as a constructive instance (compiles, runs, passes step-checker) but does NOT gate G28 on it.
- **No manifold-Hörmander hybrid in v3.1.** The sub-Riemannian (Carnot-Carathéodory) metric on a Hörmander generator has unbounded sectional curvature, violating the `BoundedGeometryManifold<F>` hypothesis B1. The hybrid (sub-Riemannian heat on a smooth manifold) is open math; defer indefinitely.
- **One opt-in `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` impl in v3.1.** The fourth v3.x opt-in (after the v3.0 DiffusionChernoff K=2, Diffusion4thChernoff K=4, TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff K=6). Higher-K hypoelliptic opt-ins (K ≥ 3) depend on resolving the Festschrift §3 problem.
- **Single-precision (`F = f32`) NOT validated for hypoelliptic kernels in v3.1.** The closed-form Kolmogorov kernel involves cancellations sensitive to f32 truncation error; G28 / G29 / T_HORM all gate at f64 precision. f32 backends compile via the Generic-over-Float trait surface but are NOT gated.

### §28.8 — References

- L. Hörmander, *Hypoelliptic second order differential equations*, **Acta Mathematica** 119:1 (1967), pp. 147-171. — §1 Theorem 1.1 (the bracket-generating condition; foundational citation for §28.2). The library reproduces only the STATEMENT; the proof of Theorem 1.1 lives in the cited paper.
