## §29 — Quantum graphs Kirchhoff vertex condition (v3.1, ADR-0078, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §29.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v2.1 graph kernels (`GraphHeatChernoff<F>`, `MagnusGraphChernoff<F>`, `GraphHeat6thChernoff<F>` — math.md §12 / §19 / §20) operate on the **discrete graph Laplacian** $L_G : \mathbb{R}^V \to \mathbb{R}^V$: one scalar per vertex, no edge structure. These are mathematically distinct from **quantum graphs** (Kuchment 2004) which equip each edge $e_i$ with a *continuum* PDE (typically $-\tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x^2$) coupled through a *vertex condition* at each branch point. Quantum graphs are the canonical setting for wave propagation on networks (Kirchhoff's laws lift to PDE), thin-domain limits of waveguides (Exner-Post 2009), and spectral theory of metric trees (Friedlander 2005).

v3.1 ships `QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F>` — the **first** quantum-graph kernel class in the library — completing the graph-completeness arc (ordinary graphs in v2.1 → quantum graphs in v3.1). The algorithm is: per Chernoff step, evolve each edge independently as a 1D heat semigroup (using the existing `ShiftChernoff1D<F>` v0.1.0 kernel), then project the per-vertex multi-edge values onto the Kirchhoff-satisfying subspace via an orthogonal projection at each vertex. Order is 1 (matching `ShiftChernoff1D`); order-2 via per-edge `DiffusionChernoff` defers to v3.2.

### §29.2 — Kirchhoff vertex condition + closed-form orthogonal projection (CITATION — Kuchment 2004 §3.2)

**Definition 29.1 (Kirchhoff vertex condition).** Let $\Gamma$ be a metric graph with vertex set $V$ and edge set $E$. For each edge $e \in E$, let $\partial_x u(v, e)$ denote the *outward* derivative of $u$ along $e$ at the vertex $v$ (positive into the vertex). At each vertex $v \in V$ of degree $d_v := |\{e \in E : v \in e\}|$, the Kirchhoff condition imposes:
- (V1) Continuity: $u$ is single-valued at $v$ — all $d_v$ edge values agree.
- (V2) Conservation of derivative flux: $\sum_{e \ni v} \partial_x u(v, e) = 0$.

A function $u$ satisfies the Kirchhoff condition at $v$ iff $u|_v \in \mathcal{K}_v$ where $\mathcal{K}_v \subset \mathbb{R}^{d_v}$ is the Kirchhoff subspace — a $(d_v - 1)$-dimensional subspace.

**Proposition 29.1 (Kirchhoff orthogonal projector, NORMATIVE library — closed-form derivation, T_QG sub-check 1).** The orthogonal projector $P_v : \mathbb{R}^{d_v} \to \mathcal{K}_v$ in the standard basis of edge-endpoint values has the closed form
$$
P_v \;=\; I_{d_v} \;-\; \frac{1}{d_v}\,\mathbf{1}_{d_v}\mathbf{1}_{d_v}^T, \tag{29.1}
$$
where $I_{d_v}$ is the $d_v \times d_v$ identity and $\mathbf{1}_{d_v}$ is the all-ones $d_v$-vector. The factor $\tfrac{1}{d_v}\mathbf{1}_{d_v}\mathbf{1}_{d_v}^T$ subtracts the vertex-mean from each edge endpoint; the residual is the Kirchhoff component (continuity is realised by all edges having the same vertex-mean, and the flux-conservation is automatic because the average of residuals is zero).

**Proof sketch (verified symbolically by T_QG sub-check 1)**: $P_v^2 = P_v$ (idempotent — orthogonal projector); $P_v \mathbf{1}_{d_v} = 0$ (kills the continuity-violation component because $\mathbf{1}_{d_v}^T \mathbf{1}_{d_v} = d_v$); $\sum_k (P_v y)_k = 0$ (the derivative-flux row sum is zero by direct computation using $\sum_k (\mathbf{1}\mathbf{1}^T y)_k = d_v \sum_k y_k$). Full symbolic derivation in `scripts/verify_quantum_graph_kirchhoff.py` (T_QG gate).

**Note on equation 29.1**: the closed form (29.1) is the SIMPLEST Kirchhoff projector — it enforces continuity (V1) and *implicitly* enforces flux conservation (V2) via the residual being mean-zero. Equivalent equivalent presentations exist in the literature with explicit flux-conservation terms (e.g., $P = I - \tfrac{1}{d}\mathbf{1}\mathbf{1}^T - \tfrac{1}{d}J$ where $J$ is the all-ones matrix); these are mathematically equivalent because the additional $J$ term is already absorbed in the projection composition. v3.1 uses (29.1).

### §29.3 — Algorithmic semantics (NORMATIVE library)

The wrapper `QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F>` realises the Kirchhoff heat semigroup via the per-step algorithm:

```
QuantumGraphHeatChernoff::apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch):
  // Phase 1 — Edgewise heat (per-edge independent ShiftChernoff1D step).
  for e in 0..n_edges:
      edge_kernels[e].apply_into(τ, src.edge_signal(e), dst.edge_signal_mut(e), scratch)?;
  // After phase 1, dst contains the edgewise heat-evolved signal but the
  // per-vertex multi-edge endpoint values are NOT in the Kirchhoff subspace.

  // Phase 2 — Per-vertex Kirchhoff projection (orthogonal, idempotent).
  for v in 0..n_vertices:
      let d := vertices[v].degree;
      let mut endpoint_buf = scratch.borrow_vec(d);
      // Gather: collect the d endpoint values at vertex v.
      for (k, e) in vertices[v].incident_edges.iter().enumerate():
          endpoint_buf[k] := dst.edge_endpoint_value(e, vertex_v_side_of_e);
      // Project: apply P_v from (29.1) — single GEMV at degree d.
      let mut projected_buf = scratch.borrow_vec(d);
      gemv(&vertices[v].projection_matrix, &endpoint_buf, &mut projected_buf);
      // Scatter: write the projected values back.
      for (k, e) in vertices[v].incident_edges.iter().enumerate():
          dst.set_edge_endpoint_value(e, vertex_v_side_of_e, projected_buf[k]);
  // After phase 2, dst is in the Kirchhoff subspace (verified by G30 spectral test).
```

**Per-step cost**: $\sum_e \text{cost}(\text{ShiftChernoff1D edge } e) + \sum_v O(d_v^2)$ — dominated by the per-edge work for typical graphs ($d_v \le 8$).

**Order**: 1 (matches `ShiftChernoff1D::order()`; the orthogonal projection is idempotent and exact at every step, so it doesn't degrade the order). Order-2 via per-edge `DiffusionChernoff` defers to v3.2.

**Growth**: $(1, 0)$ — the per-edge heat kernel is contractive on each edge; the Kirchhoff projection is a contraction (orthogonal projector); the composition is contractive on $L^2(\Gamma)$.

### §29.4 — Reference graphs and Friedlander oracle (NORMATIVE library — G30 setup)

**G30 path-graph oracle (Friedlander 2005 *Annales Inst. Fourier* §2)**: the path graph $P_3$ has 3 vertices $v_1, v_2, v_3$ and 2 edges $e_1 = (v_1, v_2)$, $e_2 = (v_2, v_3)$ of equal length $\ell = 1$. At the boundary vertices $v_1, v_3$ (degree 1), the Kirchhoff condition reduces to Neumann ($\partial_x u(v_1, e_1) = 0$); at the middle vertex $v_2$ (degree 2), it enforces continuity + flux conservation (continuity of the derivative across the vertex).

The Kirchhoff heat semigroup on $P_3$ has spectrum $\{\lambda_k\}_{k=0}^\infty$ where $\lambda_k = \tfrac{1}{2}(k\pi/(2\ell))^2 = \tfrac{k^2 \pi^2}{8}$ for $k = 0, 1, 2, \ldots$; the corresponding eigenmodes $\phi_k$ on $[0, 2\ell] = [0, 2]$ (parameterising the path by arc length) are $\phi_k(s) = \cos(k\pi s / (2\ell)) = \cos(k\pi s / 2)$ (the standard Neumann eigenmodes on a length-2 interval).

The first 4 eigenmodes used by G30 are:
- $\phi_0(s) = 1 / \sqrt{2}$ (constant ground state)
- $\phi_1(s) = \cos(\pi s / 2)$
- $\phi_2(s) = \cos(\pi s)$
- $\phi_3(s) = \cos(3\pi s / 2)$

with eigenvalues $\lambda_0 = 0$, $\lambda_1 = \pi^2/8$, $\lambda_2 = \pi^2/2$, $\lambda_3 = 9\pi^2/8$. T_QG sub-check 2 derives these symbolically.

### §29.5 — Acceptance gates (G30 + T_QG — NORMATIVE)

- **G30 (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0078): First 4 Friedlander eigenmodes on path graph reconstructed with error ≤ 1e-3 at n=64.** Setup:
  ```rust
  let edge_endpoints = vec![(0usize, 1usize), (1usize, 2usize)];   // path P_3
  let edge_lengths   = vec![1.0_f64, 1.0_f64];                       // unit edges
  let graph = QuantumGraph::<f64>::new(edge_endpoints, edge_lengths, 64)?;
  let kernel = QuantumGraphHeatChernoff::<f64>::new(graph.clone())?;
  ```
  For each of the first 4 eigenmodes $\phi_k$ ($k = 0, 1, 2, 3$):
  1. Sample $\phi_k$ on the per-edge grids to construct initial datum `f_0 := QuantumGraphSignal::from_eigenmode(graph, phi_k)`.
  2. Evolve via `Evolver::new(kernel.clone(), 64)?.evolve(T, &f_0)?` at $T = 0.1$.
  3. Compute the expected value $u_{\mathrm{ref}}^{(k)} := e^{-\lambda_k T} \phi_k$ on the per-edge grids.
  4. Verify $\|u^{(k)} - u_{\mathrm{ref}}^{(k)}\|_\infty \le 10^{-3}$.

  All 4 sub-checks (one per eigenmode) MUST pass. The error budget $10^{-3}$ accounts for the per-edge `ShiftChernoff1D` order-1 global error at $n = 64$ with $T = 0.1$ (typical heat-equation time-scale on a unit-length edge). The test ALSO verifies that the eigenmode structure is preserved (the post-evolution signal remains in the span of $\{\phi_k\}$ up to the error budget) — a structural property of the Kirchhoff projector.

  Test file: `tests/quantum_graph_eigenmode.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v3.1 release.

- **T_QG (NORMATIVE sympy — ADR-0078): Kirchhoff projection identity + first 4 Friedlander eigenmodes derivation.** Sympy verification — 3 sub-checks (all mandatory):
  1. **(T_QG.kirchhoff_projector_identity)** For $d \in \{2, 3, 4, 8\}$, construct $P_d := I_d - \tfrac{1}{d}\mathbf{1}_d \mathbf{1}_d^T$ from (29.1) and verify symbolically: (a) $P_d$ is symmetric ($P_d^T = P_d$); (b) $P_d$ is idempotent ($P_d^2 = P_d$); (c) $\text{rank}(P_d) = d - 1$ (one continuity-violation direction killed); (d) $P_d \mathbf{1}_d = 0$ (mean-zero is preserved). All 4 sub-properties must hold for all 4 degrees.
  2. **(T_QG.friedlander_eigenmodes)** Derive the first 4 eigenmodes $\phi_0, \ldots, \phi_3$ of the path $P_3$ Kirchhoff heat operator symbolically via Neumann boundary conditions at the endpoints + continuity at the middle vertex. Verify $\phi_k(s) = \cos(k\pi s / 2)$ and eigenvalues $\lambda_k = k^2\pi^2/8$ as the closed form. Verify the eigenmodes are pairwise $L^2$-orthogonal: $\int_0^2 \phi_j(s) \phi_k(s)\,ds = 0$ for $j \ne k$. The reference values feed into G30's $u_{\mathrm{ref}}^{(k)}$ table.
  3. **(T_QG.projection_scalar_compatibility)** For a degree-2 vertex (the middle vertex of $P_3$), verify that the Kirchhoff projector $P_2$ from (29.1) applied to a continuous-but-flux-nonzero endpoint pair $(u_L, u_R)$ produces an endpoint pair whose discrete flux is zero (i.e., the projected $u_R - u_L = 0$). This is the *scalar* sanity check that the algorithm's per-vertex projection step actually enforces the V1 + V2 conditions on the discrete grid — bridges the symbolic projector identity to the runtime algorithm.

  Script: `scripts/verify_quantum_graph_kirchhoff.py` (new file, ~180 LoC, ships in v3.1 Wave C engineer). MUST print exactly `T_QG PASS` on success (all 3 sub-checks pass) or `T_QG FAIL: <reason>` on failure (any sub-check fails). Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_v2_*.py` + `verify_zeta4_correction.py` + the v3.1 sibling `verify_hormander_kolmogorov.py`. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; safe for CI without `slow-tests`. Failure BLOCKS v3.1 release.

- **G31 (RELEASE_BLOCKING — Issue #15 fix): Star-graph (degree ≥ 3) mass conservation ≤ 3% drift.** Added in v7.0.1 to close the regression gap left by G30 (which only tests a path topology).

  **Root cause (Issue #15, confirmed by instrumentation):** `build_combined_kernel` originally enabled the combined-domain fast path `[0, L_total]` for ALL uniform graphs (equal edge lengths and grid sizes). A star graph IS uniform but its topology is NOT isometric to a single interval: concatenating $d$ arms into $[0, d \cdot L]$ co-locates arm $k$'s outer endpoint (leaf) with arm $k{+}1$'s inner endpoint (hub) in the combined buffer — vertices that are physically distinct. The 1D heat equation then transports heat across that spurious junction, injecting fictitious mass near the hub (24%–30% drift at $T=0.8$).

  **Fix:** A private predicate `is_path_topology` returns `true` iff every vertex has degree $\le 2$. `build_combined_kernel` gates on `is_path_topology`: stars and general branching graphs fall back to the per-edge kernel path, which is always correct. Path graphs (all-degree-2) continue to use the combined-domain kernel.

  Setup (3 sub-checks, all MUST pass):
  ```rust
  // G31a — Path-4 baseline (per-edge path, degree-2 only)
  let graph = QuantumGraph::<f64>::path(4, 1.0, 40)?;
  // G31b — Star-3 hub-degree-3
  let graph = QuantumGraph::<f64>::star(3, 1.0, 40)?;
  // G31c — Star-4 hub-degree-4
  let graph = QuantumGraph::<f64>::star(4, 1.0, 40)?;
  ```
  For each: set IC = 1 on first edge, 0 elsewhere; evolve $T = 0.8$ with 80 Chernoff steps; verify $|\text{mass}(T) - \text{mass}(0)| / \text{mass}(0) \le 3\%$ (trapezoidal arc-length integral).

  Test file: `tests/g31_star_mass_conservation.rs`. All 3 sub-checks MUST pass. Failure BLOCKS release.

### §29.6 — `QuantumGraph<F>` + `KirchhoffVertex<F>` + `QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F>` (NORMATIVE library — public API)

```rust
pub struct QuantumGraph<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    n_vertices: usize,
    n_edges: usize,
    edge_endpoints: Vec<(usize, usize)>,
    edge_lengths: Vec<F>,
    edge_grids: Vec<Grid1D<F>>,
    vertex_adjacency: Vec<Vec<usize>>,
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> QuantumGraph<F> {
    pub fn new(
        edge_endpoints: Vec<(usize, usize)>,
        edge_lengths: Vec<F>,
        edge_n_grid_points: usize,
    ) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

pub struct KirchhoffVertex<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    vertex_index: usize,
    degree: usize,
    incident_edges: Vec<usize>,
    projection_matrix: Vec<F>,           // row-major degree × degree (from equation 29.1)
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> KirchhoffVertex<F> {
    pub fn new(graph: &QuantumGraph<F>, vertex_index: usize) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

pub struct QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    graph: QuantumGraph<F>,
    vertices: Vec<KirchhoffVertex<F>>,
    edge_kernels: Vec<ShiftChernoff1D<F>>,
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F> {
    pub fn new(graph: QuantumGraph<F>) -> Result<Self, SemiflowError>;
}

pub struct QuantumGraphSignal<F: SemiflowFloat = f64> {
    per_edge: Vec<GridFn1D<F>>,
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> State<F> for QuantumGraphSignal<F> {
    // axpy, scale, norm_sup, zeroed_like via per-edge delegation
}

impl<F: SemiflowFloat> ChernoffFunction<F> for QuantumGraphHeatChernoff<F> {
    type S = QuantumGraphSignal<F>;
    fn apply_into(
        &self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, dst: &mut Self::S,
        scratch: &mut ScratchPool<F>,
    ) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        // Per math §29.3 — phase 1 edgewise heat + phase 2 vertex projection
        todo!()
    }
    fn order(&self) -> u32 { 1 }            // matches ShiftChernoff1D
    fn growth(&self) -> Growth<F> { Growth { multiplier: F::one(), omega: F::zero() } }
}
```

### §29.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Order-1 only in v3.1.** Per-edge inner uses `ShiftChernoff1D<F>` (order 1). Order-2 via per-edge `DiffusionChernoff<F>` defers to v3.2 — requires designing a per-edge boundary policy that matches the Kirchhoff projection at the vertex (significant additional design effort; no in v3.1 marginal value beyond the structural validation).
- **Kirchhoff vertex condition only.** The δ-vertex condition ($\sum \partial_x u = \alpha u(v)$) and the δ'-vertex condition (Berkolaiko-Kuchment 2013 §1.4.2) defer to C7 Tier C. Both fit the same `QuantumGraphHeatChernoff` framework with a different projection matrix per vertex.
- **Real-valued scope only.** Quantum Schrödinger (complex-valued $\psi$ + Kirchhoff coupling for the Schrödinger flux) defers to v4.x+ once `SemiflowComplex` is available.
- **Limited gate coverage in v3.1.** Only the path graph $P_3$ (3 vertices, 2 edges) and the first 4 eigenmodes are gated. Star graphs, tree graphs, ring graphs defer to v3.2 (the Friedlander oracle extends symbolically; the engineer cost is moderate).
- **Single-precision (`F = f32`) NOT validated.** The Kirchhoff projector (29.1) is well-conditioned, but the spectral-decomposition reconstruction at $n = 64$ with $T = 0.1$ has not been validated at f32 precision. f32 backends compile via the Generic-over-Float trait surface but are NOT gated.
- **Equal-length-edges assumption in `QuantumGraph::new`.** The v3.1 constructor takes a single `edge_n_grid_points: usize` for all edges (same grid resolution). Variable per-edge grid resolution defers to v3.2; not needed for the v3.1 G30 gate (path-graph edges are equal-length by construction).

### §29.8 — References

- L. Friedlander, *Genericity of simple eigenvalues for a metric graph*, **Annales de l'Institut Fourier** 55:1 (2005), pp. 199-211. — §2 (the spectral theory of the metric-graph Laplacian; cited for §29.4 G30 oracle). The first 4 eigenmodes of the path graph $P_3$ derived in §29.4 follow Friedlander's symbolic construction.
- P. Kuchment, *Quantum graphs: an introduction and a brief survey*, **Waves in Random Media** 14 (2004), pp. S107-S128. — §1 (motivation), §3.2 (Kirchhoff vertex condition; cited for §29.2 Definition 29.1). The canonical survey of the quantum-graph framework adopted by v3.1.
- P. Exner, O. Post, *Convergence of spectra of graph-like thin manifolds*, **Journal of Geometric Analysis** 18 (2008), pp. 113-145. — Cited for vertex-condition theory motivation (Kirchhoff arises as thin-manifold limit of waveguide spectra). Physical context for the v3.1 vertex condition choice.
- G. Berkolaiko, P. Kuchment, *Introduction to Quantum Graphs*, **AMS Mathematical Surveys and Monographs** 186 (2013). — §1.4.2 (δ-vertex / δ'-vertex extensions; cited in `QuantumGraph<F>` rustdoc for the deferred-to-C7 extensions).
- v0.1.0 ShiftChernoff1D precedent: math.md §1-§2 (per-edge inner kernel; reused without modification).
- v2.1 ordinary-graph pillar precedent: math.md §12 (the `GraphSignal<F>` + `GraphHeatChernoff<F>` structural model for the v3.1 quantum-graph state type design).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 6. — Foundational Chernoff theorem (already cited in §1).

## §30 — Complex semigroups and Schrödinger Option B (v4.0, ADR-0079, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §30.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v2.2 Schrödinger kernel (`schrodinger.rs`, ADR-0057) realised the Schrödinger semigroup $\{e^{-itH}\}_{t \in \mathbb{R}}$ for the kinetic-plus-potential Hamiltonian $H = -\tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x^2 + V(x)$ on a 1D grid by storing the wave function $\psi$ as a real PAIR $(\psi_{\mathrm{re}}, \psi_{\mathrm{im}}) \in \mathbb{R}^N \times \mathbb{R}^N$ — an unwrapped (`f64`, `f64`) tuple per grid point. This Option A representation was forced at v2.2 by the absence of a generic complex-arithmetic abstraction: the `SemiflowFloat<F>` bound (ADR-0025 / ADR-0026) covered only real-valued $F$, and adding `num_complex::Complex<F>` as a Chernoff state type would have required either (a) a per-method special-case in every existing kernel implementation (combinatorial — 26+ kernels), or (b) a complex-number abstraction trait that did not yet exist.

The Option A real-pair representation has three significant costs that have accumulated through v2.2 → v3.1:

1. **Per-step bookkeeping**: every Chernoff step must explicitly carry both $\psi_{\mathrm{re}}$ and $\psi_{\mathrm{im}}$ slices through `apply_into`, the scratch pool needs paired buffers, and the Crank-Nicolson kinetic step (ADR-0057 §"Mixed-precision f64-promote path") is hand-coded for the $2 \times 2$ block structure rather than expressed as a single complex matrix solve.
2. **Lifted-only quantum graphs deferred**: ADR-0078 §29.7 explicitly defers quantum-Schrödinger semigroups on metric graphs to v4.x+ "once `SemiflowComplex` is available", because the per-edge Schrödinger flux conservation at the Kirchhoff vertex is a *complex* conservation law (probability current).
3. **Future matrix-valued and rough-volatility tracks blocked**: ADR-0082 §31 (matrix-valued diffusion with potentially complex coupling) and the v4.0 HFT side-track `examples/rough_heston_markov.rs` (Bayer-Friz-Gulisashvili 2019 Markov approximation has natively complex state vectors) require complex-valued state at the trait level.

v4.0 ADR-0079 introduces `SemiflowComplex<C>` as a generic complex-arithmetic abstraction trait paralleling `SemiflowFloat<F>` (ADR-0025), and ships `SchrödingerChernoffComplex<C: SemiflowComplex>` as a SIBLING kernel to the v2.2 `SchrödingerChernoff<F: SemiflowFloat>` real-pair kernel. The v2.2 kernel is PRESERVED verbatim through v4.x (no removal; soft-deprecation via rustdoc only). The v4.0 sibling stores $\psi: \mathrm{GridFn1D}\langle C \rangle$ natively as a complex-valued grid function — one complex per grid point — and reuses the same palindromic Strang outer step (Pazy 1983 §6.4) wrapped around a single complex Crank-Nicolson kinetic step (Cheng 2008 §3.2).

### §30.2 — The `SemiflowComplex<C>` trait (NORMATIVE library)

**Definition 30.1 (Complex-arithmetic trait).** A type $C$ satisfies `SemiflowComplex<C>` iff:
- (R30.1.a) Each $z \in C$ has a real component $\Re z : \mathbb{R}_F$ and an imaginary component $\Im z : \mathbb{R}_F$ where $\mathbb{R}_F$ is a `SemiflowFloat<F>` associated type `C::Real`.
- (R30.1.b) The four field operations $+, -, \cdot, /$ are well-defined on $C$ and agree with the standard $\mathbb{C}$-arithmetic when $C = \mathbb{C}$ (i.e., when $\mathbb{R}_F = \mathbb{R}$).
- (R30.1.c) The modulus $|z| := \sqrt{(\Re z)^2 + (\Im z)^2} : \mathbb{R}_F$ is well-defined.
- (R30.1.d) The complex conjugate $\bar z$ satisfies $\Re(\bar z) = \Re z$ and $\Im(\bar z) = -\Im z$.
- (R30.1.e) The exponential $\exp(z)$ satisfies $\exp(z) = \exp(\Re z) \cdot [\cos(\Im z) + i \sin(\Im z)]$ (Euler's formula); the principal square root $\sqrt z$ satisfies $(\sqrt z)^2 = z$ on the principal branch $\arg(\sqrt z) \in (-\pi/2, \pi/2]$.
- (R30.1.f) Conversion from real: `from_real(r : C::Real) -> C` gives $\Re = r, \Im = 0$. Construction from parts: `from_parts(re, im) -> C` gives $\Re = re, \Im = im$. Polar form: `from_polar(r, theta) -> C` gives $r(\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)$.

**Reference impls shipped at v4.0**: `num_complex::Complex<f64>` and `num_complex::Complex<f32>` (the `num-complex` crate dependency is promoted from "reserved" to "direct" per ADR-0079; total `semiflow-core` deps becomes 3 / 3 cap). The trait surface allows downstream users to plug in alternative complex types (e.g., GMP-precision `arbitrary_complex::Complex`, hardware-accelerated `simd_complex::Complex4`) without modifying any Chernoff kernel.

**Note on bit-equality with Option A**: equation 30.2 below establishes the canonical Cayley-map step. When `C = num_complex::Complex<f64>` and the Option A v2.2 kernel uses the same Cayley map block-decomposed into the $(\Re, \Im)$ pair, the two representations are mathematically equivalent. At f64 precision, the byte-identity is NOT guaranteed (Option A's block-LU is hand-coded with explicit `re`/`im` ordering that may reorder a few floating-point sums vs Option B's complex-LU; the discrepancy is $\le 4$ ULP on the canonical harmonic-oscillator wave packet). This is the trade-off: byte-identity vs $\le 4$ ULP convergence on a Gaussian wave packet at $N = 512$, $T = 1.0$, $n = 128$. See §30.6 G_SCHROD_B gate.

### §30.3 — Schrödinger Option B Chernoff step (CITATION — Pazy 1983 §6.4, Cheng 2008 §3.2)

The Schrödinger semigroup $U(t) := e^{-itH}$ for $H = -\tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x^2 + V(x)$ is *unitary* on $L^2(\mathbb{R})$ (preserves the $L^2$-norm); the palindromic Strang decomposition (Pazy 1983 §6.4 — the standard reference for parabolic + hyperbolic semigroup splittings):

$$
U(\tau) \;\approx\; e^{-i\tau V/2} \,\circ\, e^{+i\tau \partial_x^2 / 2} \,\circ\, e^{-i\tau V/2} \;+\; O(\tau^3)
\tag{30.1}
$$

is order-2 in $\tau$. The inner kinetic propagator $e^{+i\tau\partial_x^2/2}$ is the unitary semigroup of the free Schrödinger equation; its discrete approximation is the standard **Cayley map** (Crank-Nicolson) on the discrete Laplacian $\Delta_h$:

$$
e^{+i\tau\Delta_h / 2} \;\approx\; \bigl(I - \tfrac{i\tau}{4}\Delta_h\bigr)^{-1} \bigl(I + \tfrac{i\tau}{4}\Delta_h\bigr)
\tag{30.2}
$$

which is the unique unitary rational approximation of order 2. The potential half-steps $e^{-i\tau V/2}$ are pointwise complex multiplications $\psi(x) \mapsto \exp(-i\tau V(x)/2) \cdot \psi(x)$.

**Option B per-step semantics** (NORMATIVE — verified by G_SCHROD_B gate at §30.6):

```
SchrödingerChernoffComplex::apply_into(τ, ψ_src, ψ_dst, scratch):
  // Step 1 — potential half-step (pointwise complex multiplication):
  for k in 0..N:
    tmp[k] = exp(-i·τ·V[k]/2) · ψ_src[k]                                    // C arithmetic
  // Step 2 — kinetic full-step (Cayley map / complex Crank-Nicolson):
  // Solve (I - (iτ/4) Δ_h) tmp2 = (I + (iτ/4) Δ_h) tmp
  rhs = (I + (iτ/4) Δ_h) · tmp                                              // complex matvec
  tmp2 = banded_complex_lu_solve(I - (iτ/4) Δ_h, rhs)                       // banded complex LU
  // Step 3 — second potential half-step:
  for k in 0..N:
    ψ_dst[k] = exp(-i·τ·V[k]/2) · tmp2[k]                                   // C arithmetic
```

The banded-LU solve in step 2 is the COMPLEX analog of the v2.2 Option A real-pair $2 \times 2$ block LU. The complex banded LU uses the same tridiagonal structure (the 5-point Laplacian stencil with reflecting BCs yields a tridiagonal $I - (i\tau/4)\Delta_h$; for higher-order Laplacian stencils the band-width is wider but the LU remains $O(N)$ work per step).

### §30.4 — Unitarity preservation (NORMATIVE library — G_SCHROD_B gate foundation)

**Proposition 30.1 (Unitarity at f64).** Let $\psi_n$ be the Option B Chernoff iterate of the Gaussian wave packet $\psi_0(x) = \pi^{-1/4} \exp(-x^2/2 + i k_0 x)$ on the harmonic-oscillator Hamiltonian $H = -\tfrac{1}{2}\partial_x^2 + \tfrac{1}{2}x^2$ at $T = 1.0$, $N = 512$, $n = 128$ palindromic Strang steps with complex Cayley map per (30.2). Then $\|\psi_n\|_2 = \|\psi_0\|_2$ to within $10^{-12}$ relative error at f64 precision.

**Proof sketch** (verified empirically by G_SCHROD_B gate): each Option B step is the composition of three unitary operators — pointwise complex multiplications of unit modulus ($|\exp(-i\tau V/2)| = 1$ pointwise) and a Cayley map of an anti-Hermitian operator ($i\Delta_h$ is anti-Hermitian iff $\Delta_h$ is symmetric, which the 5-point reflecting-BC stencil is). The composition is unitary by construction at the discrete level, modulo floating-point cancellation. The $10^{-12}$ relative budget absorbs the 128-step accumulation of f64 round-off in the complex banded-LU solve.

**Contrast with Option A**: the v2.2 real-pair representation achieves the same unitarity at the level of equation 30.2 because the real-pair $2 \times 2$ block structure is the canonical real-form representation of the complex Cayley map. However, the real-pair block LU computes the $(\Re, \Im)$ entries through a slightly different floating-point sequence: $\Re(z_1 z_2) = \Re z_1 \Re z_2 - \Im z_1 \Im z_2$ vs the complex form $\Re(z_1 z_2)$ as a single fused operation in `num_complex`. The $\le 4$ ULP discrepancy at $N = 512$, $n = 128$ is BELOW the G_SCHROD_B unitarity budget but is OBSERVABLE in byte-comparison tests (which is why G_SCHROD_B does NOT include a cross-version byte-identity sub-test — see §30.6).

### §30.5 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **Schrödinger 2D / 3D**: v4.0 ships 1D only. The 2D analog requires the 2D Cayley map $(I - (i\tau/4)\Delta_{2D,h})^{-1} (I + (i\tau/4)\Delta_{2D,h})$ where $\Delta_{2D,h}$ is the discrete 2D Laplacian. Direct LU of a 2D banded-pentadiagonal system is $O(N^2)$ per step; iterative solvers (BiCGStab on the complex system) defer to v4.x+. Beyond ADR-0057 v2.2 §"out of scope" — same blocker.
- **Quantum graphs Schrödinger**: ADR-0078 §29.7 (deferred to v4.x+ once `SemiflowComplex` is available — v4.0 ADR-0079 ships the trait; the actual quantum-Schrödinger composition `QuantumSchrödingerChernoff<C>` reusing `KirchhoffVertex<C>` with complex projector defers to v4.1+ — the projector formula (29.1) lifts unchanged to $\mathbb{C}^{d_v}$, but the per-edge Schrödinger flux conservation $\sum_e \mathrm{Im}(\bar\psi \partial_x \psi) = 0$ is a NEW conservation law that needs its own vertex condition class). **RESOLVED at v7.0.0 (ADR-0130) — and the "new vertex condition class" premise is FALSIFIED, see §30.5-bis.**

### §30.5-bis — QuantumSchrödingerChernoff on quantum graphs (v7.0.0, ADR-0130, NORMATIVE library)

Ships `QuantumSchrödingerChernoff<C>` as an additive composition reusing the EXISTING heat Kirchhoff projector $Q_v=(1/d)\mathbf{1}\mathbf{1}^T$ (math §29.1) around a complex Cayley kinetic step (§30.3). PRE-FLIGHT `scripts/verify_quantum_schrodinger.py` (executed 2026-06-06, 3/3 PASS) **falsifies the §29.7/§30.5 "needs its own vertex condition class" premise**: (1) $Q_v$ over $\mathbb{C}$ is Hermitian, idempotent, rank-1 ($d=2,3,4$) — the projector (29.1) lifts to $\mathbb{C}^{d_v}$ verbatim; (2) the per-vertex map $Q\!\cdot\!\mathrm{Cayley}\!\cdot\!Q$ is norm-preserving on the continuity subspace (the Cayley map of the anti-Hermitian $(i\tau/2)L$ is exactly unitary, $U^H U=I$ symbolic); (3) the Schrödinger probability current is IMPLIED, not independent:
$$\sum_e \mathrm{Im}(\bar\psi_e \partial_x\psi_e)\Big|_v = \mathrm{Im}\Big(\bar\psi(v)\sum_e \partial_x\psi_e\Big) = \mathrm{Im}(\bar\psi(v)\cdot 0) = 0,$$
because continuity ($Q$ forces $\psi_e(v)$ equal across edges) plus the heat-Kirchhoff derivative balance $\sum_e\partial_x\psi_e=0$ together give $J=0$. No separate vertex class is required — the heat `QuantumGraph` framework is reused unchanged with complex per-edge state. Two-half-step structure: Phase-1 per-edge complex Cayley (unitary) + Phase-2 vertex $Q$, mirroring the shipped heat kernel. Gate `G_QSCHROD`: eigenmode max_err $\le 5\times10^{-4}$ (mirror G30) or unitarity drift $\le 5\times10^{-4}$. Order-1 per-edge inheritance (order-2 per-edge deferred per §29.7); path-graph $P_3$ eigenmode gating mirrors G30. ZERO new deps. References: Kuchment 2004 §3.2 (Kirchhoff); §30.3 (complex Cayley map); Friedlander 2005 (eigenmode oracle).
- **Non-Hermitian Hamiltonians**: $H + i\Gamma(x)$ with imaginary potential (decay / absorbing BCs) is a NEW use case the Option B representation enables natively (the potential half-step becomes $\exp(-i\tau (V + i\Gamma)/2) = \exp(-i\tau V/2) \cdot \exp(\tau\Gamma/2)$ which is complex-valued of non-unit modulus). v4.0 does NOT gate non-Hermitian potentials; the kernel compiles them but G_SCHROD_B uses Hermitian $V(x) = x^2/2$.

### §30.6 — Acceptance gate G_SCHROD_B (NORMATIVE library)

**G_SCHROD_B (RELEASE_BLOCKING — Schrödinger Option B unitarity at f64)**:

Setup:
```
grid    = Grid1D::<f64>::new(-10.0, 10.0, 512)?;
V_fn    = |x: f64| 0.5 * x * x;                                  // harmonic oscillator
k0      = 2.0_f64;                                                 // mean momentum
psi_0   = |x: f64| Complex::from_polar(
              (PI.powf(-0.25)) * (-x*x/2.0).exp(),                // Gaussian envelope
              k0 * x,                                              // plane-wave phase
          );
kernel  = SchrödingerChernoffComplex::<Complex<f64>>::new(
              grid.clone(), V_fn,
          )?;
T       = 1.0_f64;
n       = 128_usize;                                               // palindromic Strang steps
```

Sweep: single value (NOT an n-sweep — this is a unitarity-preservation gate, not a convergence-rate gate).

Reference solution: the EXACT $L^2$-norm of the Gaussian wave packet is $\|\psi_0\|_2 = 1.0$ (analytic — the Gaussian normalisation $\pi^{-1/4}$ in the envelope is the standard $L^2(\mathbb{R})$ unit-norm constant; on the truncated grid $[-10, 10]$ with $\sigma = 1$, the truncation error is $< 10^{-43}$).

Gate:
```
psi_n  = Evolver::new(kernel.clone(), n)?.evolve(T, &psi_0)?;
norm_n = sqrt(sum(|psi_n[k]|² for k in 0..512) · dx);
ASSERT |norm_n - 1.0| < 1e-12;
```

Test file: `tests/schrodinger_complex_unitarity.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). Failure BLOCKS v4.0 release.

**Sub-test 2 (Option A / Option B convergence cross-check, ADVISORY)**: at $N = 512$, $T = 1.0$, $n = 128$, the sup-norm $\|\psi_n^{(A)} - \psi_n^{(B)}\|_\infty \le 4$ ULP $\approx 8.88 \times 10^{-16}$. This sub-test is ADVISORY (not RELEASE_BLOCKING) — it documents the cross-representation discrepancy. Failure does NOT block v4.0 but DOES trigger an investigation: the $\le 4$ ULP budget is empirically derived from the v2.2 real-pair LU vs `num_complex` LU floating-point sequence comparison; any larger discrepancy indicates a regression in either Option A or Option B.

### §30.7 — References

- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to Partial Differential Equations*, **Applied Mathematical Sciences** 44, Springer 1983. — §6.4 (operator-splitting decomposition of contractive semigroups; foundational for the palindromic Strang decomposition equation 30.1).
- Y. Cheng, *A Survey of Recent Developments in Schrödinger Equation*, **Acta Math. Sci.** 28:2 (2008), pp. 268-282. — §3.2 (Crank-Nicolson Cayley map as unitary rational approximation; foundational for equation 30.2).
- K.-J. Engel, R. Nagel, *One-Parameter Semigroups for Linear Evolution Equations*, **Graduate Texts in Mathematics** 194, Springer 2000. — §IV.6 (unitary semigroups on Hilbert space; cross-reference for §30.4 unitarity).
- v2.2 Schrödinger Option A precedent: math.md §17 (the real-pair `(psi_re, psi_im)` representation; ADR-0057). Option B in §30 is the natively-complex SIBLING.
- ADR-0079 (this section's contract authority; references back to §30.1-§30.6 verbatim).
- ADR-0078 §29.7 (deferred quantum-Schrödinger track; §30 unblocks the trait foundation but the quantum-Schrödinger composition itself defers to v4.1+).
- Reserved (BACKLOG): future paper draft on Option A vs Option B convergence properties; not part of v4.0 contract.

---

## §31 — Point evaluation iterative recursion (v4.0, ADR-0080, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §31.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v2.x library API consistently materialises the full Chernoff iterate $(F(\tau/n))^n f$ as a fully-discretised state $\mathrm{GridFn}\langle F \rangle$ (1D), $\mathrm{GridFn2D}\langle F \rangle$ (2D), $\mathrm{GridFn3D}\langle F \rangle$ (3D), or $\mathrm{QuantumGraphSignal}\langle F \rangle$ (metric graph). For applications that need the FUNCTION VALUE at a SINGLE POINT — e.g., a sample of the heat kernel at $(x_0, t_0)$ in a Monte-Carlo importance-sampling context, or a single evaluation of the manifold heat kernel at a tangent-space point in a Bayesian-inference setting — this is wasteful: the cost is $O(N)$ in storage and $O(N \cdot n)$ in compute per evaluation, where $N$ is the spatial grid size and $n$ is the number of Chernoff steps, regardless of how few points are actually queried.

The v3.0 ApproximationSubspace trait (ADR-0073) included a STUB `PointEval<F>` trait that returned `Unsupported` from every method — placeholder for future v4.0+ work pending the use cases. Two use cases now drive the API:

1. **v2.8 manifold Chernoff (ADR-0071)**: pointwise heat kernel evaluation on a Riemannian manifold $M$ at a tangent-space point $x \in T_{x_0}M$. The Chernoff approximation lives on the full discretised manifold mesh; evaluating at one tangent-space point requires only a localised piece of the Chernoff iterate.
2. **v3.1 Hörmander hypoelliptic (ADR-0077)**: pointwise fundamental-solution evaluation at phase-space point $(x, v) \in \mathbb{R}^2$ for Kolmogorov 1934 step-2 Carnot. The full phase-space mesh is $O(N^2)$ for accurate convergence; a single eval at one $(x_0, v_0)$ point should cost $O(\mathrm{poly}(n))$ not $O(N^2 \cdot n)$.

v4.0 ADR-0080 promotes `PointEval<F>` from stub to a first-class trait with bound-stack iterative pointwise evaluation. The trait surface is:

```rust
pub trait PointEval<F: SemiflowFloat>: ChernoffFunction<F> {
    /// Evaluate (F(τ))^n applied to source, sampled at point x.
    /// Bound-stack iterative — O(poly(n)) compute, O(poly(n)) auxiliary storage.
    fn eval_at(&self, tau: F, src: &Self::S, x: &[F], n_steps: u32) -> Result<F, SemiflowError>;
}
```

with backend-specific O(n) implementations for the four use-case kernels: `DiffusionChernoff`, `ShiftChernoff1D`, `ManifoldChernoff`, `HypoellipticChernoff`, `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND` (the v4.0 ADR-0081 d-D shift backend).

### §31.2 — Bound-stack iterative recursion (NORMATIVE library)

For a Chernoff function $F(\tau)$ that admits a *kernel representation* $(F(\tau) f)(x) = \int K(x, y; \tau) f(y) \, dy$, the iterated application has the integral form

$$
((F(\tau))^n f)(x_0) \;=\; \int \cdots \int K(x_0, x_1; \tau) K(x_1, x_2; \tau) \cdots K(x_{n-1}, x_n; \tau) f(x_n) \, dx_1 \cdots dx_n.
\tag{31.1}
$$

The naive evaluation of (31.1) by direct $n$-fold quadrature is $O(q^n)$ where $q$ is the per-axis quadrature order — exponential in $n$ and catastrophic for $n \ge 20$. The **bound-stack iterative** algorithm reduces this to $O(n \cdot q)$ by exploiting the *Markov property* of the kernel: the integrand at step $k$ depends only on the result at step $k - 1$, not on the entire path.

**Algorithm 31.1 (Bound-stack point eval, NORMATIVE library)**:

```
PointEval::eval_at(τ, f₀, x₀, n):
  // Single-point bound-stack iterative — O(n · q) compute, O(q) storage.
  // Where q is the per-step quadrature order (kernel-specific).

  // Step 1 — initialise auxiliary state at the query point x₀.
  let mut aux: BoundStack<F> = kernel_init(x₀, &f₀);             // backend-specific
                                                                  // typically aux.len() = O(q)

  // Step 2 — iterate n Chernoff steps backward from x₀.
  for k in 1..=n:
    // The kernel at step k contributes a per-axis quadrature update on `aux`.
    kernel_step_backward(τ, &mut aux, k);                          // O(q) work per step

  // Step 3 — reduce the final auxiliary state to a scalar.
  kernel_reduce(&aux, &f₀)                                         // backend-specific, O(q) work
```

The per-backend `kernel_init`, `kernel_step_backward`, `kernel_reduce` triple is the implementation of the kernel-specific Markov-property exploitation. For each of the four v4.0 backends:

**Backend A — DiffusionChernoff (1D)**: The diffusion kernel $K(x, y; \tau) = (2\pi\tau a(x))^{-1/2} \exp(-(x-y)^2 / (4\tau a(x)))$ is Gaussian with mean $x$ and variance $2\tau a(x)$. The bound-stack iterative reduces to a single 1D Gaussian quadrature at each step; $q = $ 5-point Gauss-Hermite suffices for f64 precision. `aux` is the 5-point quadrature node values; `kernel_step_backward` advances the variance by $2\tau a(x_{\mathrm{node}})$.

**Backend B — ShiftChernoff1D**: identical to Backend A but with constant $a$. The aux state is a 5-point Gauss-Hermite quadrature evaluated against the v0.1.0 shift-kernel closed-form Gaussian; the per-step backward is a single variance update.

**Backend C — ManifoldChernoff (v2.8 A4)**: The manifold heat kernel localises to $T_{x_0}M$ via the exponential map. The bound-stack aux state is a $(q_{\mathrm{tangent}})^{D_M}$-point quadrature on $T_{x_0}M$ where $D_M$ is the manifold dimension; the per-step backward is a parallel-transport update along the geodesic from $x_0$ to the previous-step quadrature node (geodesic spray cached at construction time). For $D_M = 2$ and $q_{\mathrm{tangent}} = 5$, the aux has 25 entries.

**Backend D — HypoellipticChernoff (v3.1 A3)**: The Hörmander hypoelliptic generator $L = X_0 + \tfrac{1}{2} \sum X_k^2$ has a step-2 Carnot fundamental solution that is Gaussian on the *graded* tangent space (Folland 1975 §2.3). The bound-stack aux is the graded-tangent quadrature on $\mathbb{R}^{D}$ where $D = \dim M$ is the phase-space dimension; the per-step backward is the Strang-Hörmander palindromic update of equation 28.4 applied to the quadrature nodes. For $D = 2$ (Kolmogorov phase space) and $q = 5^2 = 25$ Gauss-Hermite tensor nodes, the aux has 25 entries.

**Backend E — AnisotropicShiftChernoffND (v4.0 A2, see §32)**: The d-dimensional anisotropic shift kernel is Gaussian-on-$\mathbb{R}^D$ with covariance $2\tau A(x_0)$ where $A(x_0)$ is the $D \times D$ symmetric-positive-definite diffusion tensor at $x_0$. The bound-stack aux is the tensor-product Gauss-Hermite quadrature on $\mathbb{R}^D$; for $D \le 4$ this is closed-form O(q^D) per step. For $D \ge 5$, the v4.0.0 release ships a `MonteCarlo` fallback path with $q$ replaced by the MC sample count.

### §31.3 — Byte-identity contract with full-grid (NORMATIVE library — G_POINTEVAL gate foundation)

**Proposition 31.1 (Byte-identity, NORMATIVE — G_POINTEVAL).** Let $F$ be a `ChernoffFunction<F>` that implements `PointEval<F>` per the algorithm of §31.2. For every $f_0 \in $ `Self::S`, every $x_0$ in the kernel's grid support, every $\tau > 0$, and every $n \ge 1$:

$$
\bigl(F.\mathrm{eval\_at}(\tau, f_0, x_0, n)\bigr) \;\equiv_{f64}\; \bigl((F.\mathrm{apply\_into}^n f_0).\mathrm{sample}(x_0)\bigr)
\tag{31.2}
$$

where $\equiv_{f64}$ denotes byte-identity at IEEE 754 f64 precision (the two floating-point values have identical bit-patterns; `f64::to_bits()` equality).

**Verification**: G_POINTEVAL gate (§31.4) tests (31.2) on the four v4.0 PointEval backends (DiffusionChernoff, ShiftChernoff1D, ManifoldChernoff, HypoellipticChernoff, AnisotropicShiftChernoffND) at canonical test data with $\tau = T/n$ for $T = 0.5$, $n = 64$, on grid sizes appropriate to each backend.

**Note on byte-identity vs $\le 4$ ULP**: byte-identity (31.2) is strictly stronger than the v2.2 ADR-0059 graph-binding $\le 3$ ULP gate; it is achievable here because the bound-stack iterative algorithm of §31.2, when implemented faithfully, computes EXACTLY the same floating-point reductions as the full-grid path SAMPLED at the query point. Any deviation indicates an implementation bug in the bound-stack iterator. The byte-identity contract is the basis for the v4.0 testing strategy: if `eval_at` returns byte-identical to `apply_into^n . sample`, the iterator is correct.

### §31.4 — Acceptance gate G_POINTEVAL (NORMATIVE library)

**G_POINTEVAL (RELEASE_BLOCKING — byte-identity on 4 kernel backends)**:

Setup (per backend):
```
// Backend A — DiffusionChernoff
grid_A     = Grid1D::<f64>::new(-10.0, 10.0, 512)?;
a_fn       = |x: f64| 1.0 + 0.5 * (x.tanh()).powi(2);
kernel_A   = DiffusionChernoff::<f64>::new(a_fn, grid_A.clone())?;
f0_A       = GridFn1D::<f64>::from_fn(&grid_A, |x| (-x*x).exp());

// Backend B — ManifoldChernoff (Sphere2)
sphere     = Sphere2::<f64>::new();
mesh_B     = sphere.icosahedral_mesh(64)?;
kernel_B   = ManifoldChernoff::<Sphere2<f64>, f64>::new(sphere, mesh_B.clone())?;
f0_B       = ManifoldFn::<f64>::from_fn(&mesh_B, |p| harmonic_y_2_0(p));

// Backend C — HypoellipticChernoff (KolmogorovPhaseSpace)
grid_C     = GridND::<f64, 2>::new([-5.0, -5.0], [5.0, 5.0], [128, 128])?;
x0_drift   = Box::new(KolmogorovPhaseSpace::<f64>::x0_drift());
x_diff     = [Box::new(KolmogorovPhaseSpace::<f64>::x1_diffusion())];
kernel_C   = HypoellipticChernoff::<f64, 2, 1>::new(x0_drift, x_diff, grid_C.clone())?;
f0_C       = GridFnND::<f64, 2>::from_fn(&grid_C, |(x, v)| (-(x*x+v*v)/2.0).exp());

// Backend D — AnisotropicShiftChernoffND (d=2)
grid_D     = GridND::<f64, 2>::new([-5.0, -5.0], [5.0, 5.0], [128, 128])?;
a_ij       = const_anisotropic_2x2(1.0, 0.5, 0.5, 1.0);  // [[1, 0.5], [0.5, 1]]
kernel_D   = AnisotropicShiftChernoffND::<f64, 2>::new(a_ij, ..., grid_D.clone())?;
f0_D       = GridFnND::<f64, 2>::from_fn(&grid_D, |(x, y)| (-(x*x+y*y)).exp());
```

Per-backend test:
```
T = 0.5_f64;
n = 64_u32;
tau = T / (n as f64);

// Sample query point: the grid centre for each backend.
let x_query = grid_centre_of(kernel.grid());

// Full-grid path:
let full_grid_state = (0..n).fold(f0.clone(), |acc, _| {
    let mut dst = acc.clone();
    let mut pool = ScratchPool::<f64>::new();
    kernel.apply_into(tau, &acc, &mut dst, &mut pool).unwrap();
    dst
});
let full_grid_at_x = full_grid_state.sample(&x_query);

// PointEval path:
let pe_at_x = kernel.eval_at(tau, &f0, &x_query, n).unwrap();

// Gate:
ASSERT pe_at_x.to_bits() == full_grid_at_x.to_bits();
```

Test file: `tests/point_eval_byte_identity.rs` (new file, feature `slow-tests`). 5 sub-tests (one per backend). Failure of ANY sub-test BLOCKS v4.0 release.

### §31.5 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **`eval_at` for grid-only kernels** (`Strang2D`, `Diffusion4thChernoff`, `Magnus*`): these kernels lack a kernel representation $K(x, y; \tau)$ — they are defined directly on the discretised grid via finite-difference stencils. The bound-stack iterative is not applicable; these kernels DO NOT implement `PointEval<F>` in v4.0. Users querying point values on grid-only kernels MUST materialise the full-grid state via `apply_into` and call `.sample(x)`.
- **Vectorised batch eval** (`eval_at_batch(x_queries: &[F])` returning `Vec<F>`): the same bound-stack iterative can be run in parallel across query points if the per-point auxiliary states are independent. v4.0 ships single-point only; batch eval defers to v4.1+ (incremental performance optimisation).
- **GPU offload** of the bound-stack iterator: defers indefinitely (out of `no_std + alloc` scope; would require WGPU or CUDA crates that are not in the dep budget).
- **Adjoint `eval_at` for backward Chernoff** (point-evaluation of the dual semigroup): defers to v5.0+ Tier C. The bound-stack iterative is forward-only in v4.0.

### §31.6 — References

- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025). — §"Remark 9" (the original observation that pointwise evaluation admits a bound-stack iterative algorithm avoiding the $O(q^n)$ tree). Cited for §31.2 Algorithm 31.1.
- G. B. Folland, *Subelliptic estimates and function spaces on nilpotent Lie groups*, **Arkiv för Matematik** 13 (1975), pp. 161-207. — §2.3 (graded-tangent-space fundamental solutions for step-2 Carnot; cited for §31.2 Backend D).
- v2.8 manifold Chernoff: math.md §24 (the localised $T_{x_0}M$ evaluation pattern; cited for §31.2 Backend C).
- v3.1 Hörmander hypoelliptic: math.md §28 (the Kolmogorov phase-space fundamental solution; cited for §31.2 Backend D).
- v3.0 ApproximationSubspace trait: math.md §26 (the original stub PointEval trait; this §31 promotes the stub to first-class).
- ADR-0080 (this section's contract authority; references back to §31.1-§31.4 verbatim).

---

## §32 — d-Dimensional anisotropic shift Chernoff (v4.0, ADR-0081, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §32.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v0.1.0 `ShiftChernoff1D<F>` (math.md §1-§2) implements the 1D anisotropic shift Chernoff per Remizov 2025 *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* 27:4 Theorem 6 formula (6), for the 1D parabolic generator $L = a(x) \partial_x^2 + b(x) \partial_x + c(x)$. The natural d-dimensional generalisation — the parabolic generator $L = \sum_{i,j} a_{ij}(x) \partial^2_{ij} + \sum_i b_i(x) \partial_i + c(x)$ on $\mathbb{R}^D$ for $D \ge 2$ — is the subject of Remizov 2025 *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* 27:4 Theorem 3 (the "Theorem 3 cousin formula" for d-D anisotropic shift Chernoff).

The v2.5+ library has 2D and 3D anisotropic kernels (`Strang2D`, `Strang3D`, `NonSeparable2DChernoff`, `AnisotropicShift2DChernoff`) but they are SPECIFIC to $D = 2$ or $D = 3$ and use COMPOSITION patterns (Strang splitting + non-separable mixed-leg + axis-lift) rather than the closed-form shift formula. v4.0 ADR-0081 ships `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND<F, const D: usize>` as the GENERIC d-dimensional kernel via the closed-form Theorem 3 cousin formula, with reference impls gated for $D \in \{2, 3, 4, 5\}$.

The d-D shift formula gives a *natively d-dimensional* approximation that does NOT decompose into per-axis steps; the closed-form Gaussian-like kernel handles arbitrary anisotropic diffusion tensors $a_{ij}(x)$ including cross-terms (off-diagonal) that the v2.5+ Strang-composition kernels handle only via the non-separable mixed-leg correction. For applications with strongly cross-coupled diffusion (e.g., d-D anisotropic Hörmander, multi-factor financial PDEs with correlated noise), the d-D shift is the *natural* primitive.

### §32.2 — d-D anisotropic Gaussian kernel (CITATION — Friedman 1964 §1.4)

**Definition 32.1 (d-D anisotropic Gaussian).** Let $A(x) = (a_{ij}(x))_{i,j=1}^D$ be a symmetric-positive-definite $D \times D$ matrix-valued function. The frozen-coefficient anisotropic Gaussian kernel at $x$ is:
$$
K_A(x; y; \tau) \;:=\; \frac{1}{(4\pi\tau)^{D/2} \sqrt{\det A(x)}} \exp\!\Bigl( -\frac{1}{4\tau} (y - x)^T A(x)^{-1} (y - x) \Bigr).
\tag{32.1}
$$

For constant $A$ (no $x$-dependence), (32.1) is the fundamental solution of the constant-coefficient anisotropic heat equation $\partial_t u = \sum a_{ij} \partial^2_{ij} u$ on $\mathbb{R}^D$ (Friedman 1964 *Partial Differential Equations of Parabolic Type* §1.4 — the canonical reference for anisotropic Gaussian fundamental solutions).

For variable $A(x)$, (32.1) is the *frozen-coefficient* Gaussian — the analog of the v0.1.0 1D shift kernel that freezes $a(x)$ at the evaluation point $x$. The variable-coefficient correction enters at order $\tau^2$ (per Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* k=2 tangency on the d-D extension); the v6.0.0 kernel ships the **order-1 baseline** (no $\tau^2$ correction — the bare frozen-coefficient kernel is order-1; the ζ²-d-D correction that would lift it to order-2 is DEFERRED, see §32.5 Note and ADR-0112). *Pre-v6 versions of this paragraph incorrectly described an "order-2 baseline"; corrected in v6.0.0.*

### §32.3 — d-D anisotropic shift Chernoff formula (CITATION — Remizov 2025 Theorem 3 cousin)

**Theorem 32.1 (d-D shift Chernoff, CITATION — Remizov 2025 Vladikavkaz Math. J. 27:4 Theorem 3 cousin formula).** Let $L = \sum_{i,j} a_{ij}(x) \partial^2_{ij} + \sum_i b_i(x) \partial_i + c(x)$ be a strictly parabolic generator on $\mathbb{R}^D$ with $A(x) := (a_{ij}(x))$ symmetric-positive-definite, $b_i \in C_b(\mathbb{R}^D)$, $c \in C_b(\mathbb{R}^D)$. Then the d-D anisotropic shift Chernoff function
$$
F_A(\tau) f(x) \;:=\; e^{\tau c(x)} \cdot \int_{\mathbb{R}^D} K_A(x; y; \tau) \, f\!\bigl(y + \tau \, b(x)\bigr) \, dy
\tag{32.2}
$$
is order-1 Chernoff-tangent to $\{e^{tL}\}_{t \ge 0}$ on the core $C^2_b(\mathbb{R}^D)$ (the bounded twice-continuously-differentiable functions). The Chernoff product $(F_A(\tau/n))^n f$ converges to $e^{\tau L} f$ at rate $O(1/n)$ uniformly on bounded subsets of $C^2_b(\mathbb{R}^D)$.

**Proof citation**: Remizov 2025 *Vladikavkaz Math. J.* 27:4 Theorem 3 (the canonical d-D Chernoff product formula for parabolic operators). The library reproduces the FORMULA (32.2) and the convergence statement; the proof lives in the cited reference.

**Discrete implementation (NORMATIVE library)**: on a uniform Cartesian grid $\mathrm{GridND}\langle F, D \rangle$ with $N$ points per axis, the integral (32.2) is approximated by tensor-product Gauss-Hermite quadrature of order $q$ per axis. The total quadrature is $q^D$ nodes per evaluation point; for $D \le 4$ and $q = 5$ (Gauss-Hermite 5-point is exact for polynomials of degree $\le 9$, sufficient for f64 precision against the Gaussian kernel), the cost is $5^D \le 625$ per evaluation point. For $D \ge 5$, the tensor-product quadrature explodes and the v4.0 kernel falls back to a sparse-grid alternative (Smolyak sparse grid — deferred to v4.1+) or the `MonteCarlo` Backend E of §31.

### §32.4 — Discrete Gauss-Hermite quadrature of the anisotropic Gaussian (NORMATIVE library)

> **v6.0.0 CORRECTION (ADR-0112).** The pre-v6 form of equation (32.3) was
> **mathematically wrong**: it omitted the $\pi^{-D/2}$ quadrature-weight
> normalisation and used the node scale $\sqrt{2\tau}$ instead of the correct
> $2\sqrt{\tau}$. With physicist Gauss-Hermite weights ($\sum_q w_q = \sqrt\pi$
> per axis), the old form gave $F_A(0) = \pi^{D/2}\,I \neq I$, violating the
> Chernoff tangency precondition $F(0)=I$ (Chernoff 1968, §2 of this document);
> the product $(F_A(\tau/n))^n$ then diverged as $\pi^{nD/2}\to\infty$. The
> re-derivation below is the authoritative replacement. See ADR-0112.

**Re-derivation (from §32.2 eq 32.1).** The discrete kernel is the
Gauss-Hermite quadrature of the continuous frozen-coefficient operator (32.2),
in which $A(x)$ is frozen at the evaluation point $x_k$ (it is the d-D analog
of the 1D shift kernel of §1, which freezes $a$ at $x$). Start from (32.2) with
the local Gaussian $K_{A(x_k)}$ of (32.1):
$$
\bigl(F_A(\tau)f\bigr)(x_k) \;=\; e^{\tau c(x_k)}\!\int_{\mathbb{R}^D}
\frac{1}{(4\pi\tau)^{D/2}\sqrt{\det A(x_k)}}
\exp\!\Bigl(-\tfrac{1}{4\tau}(y-x_k)^T A(x_k)^{-1}(y-x_k)\Bigr)\,
f\!\bigl(y+\tau b(x_k)\bigr)\,dy.
$$
Let $A(x_k)=\sigma\sigma^T$ (Cholesky, $\sigma:=\sigma_{A(x_k)}$ lower-triangular)
and substitute the whitening change of variables $y = x_k + 2\sqrt{\tau}\,\sigma\,s$,
$s\in\mathbb{R}^D$. Then $(y-x_k)^T A^{-1}(y-x_k) = 4\tau\,s^T s$, so the Gaussian
exponent collapses to $-s^Ts = -\sum_i s_i^2$, and $dy = (2\sqrt\tau)^D\det\sigma\,ds
= (2\sqrt\tau)^D\sqrt{\det A(x_k)}\,ds$. The prefactor and Jacobian combine:
$$
\frac{(2\sqrt\tau)^D\sqrt{\det A}}{(4\pi\tau)^{D/2}\sqrt{\det A}}
= \frac{(2\sqrt\tau)^D}{(4\pi\tau)^{D/2}} = \pi^{-D/2}.
$$
Hence
$$
\bigl(F_A(\tau)f\bigr)(x_k) \;=\; e^{\tau c(x_k)}\,\pi^{-D/2}
\!\int_{\mathbb{R}^D} e^{-s^Ts}\, f\!\bigl(x_k+\tau b(x_k)+2\sqrt{\tau}\,\sigma\,s\bigr)\,ds.
$$
Applying the tensor-product 5-point Gauss-Hermite rule (physicist weight
$e^{-s^2}$, nodes $\eta_{q_i}$, weights $w_{q_i}$, exact to degree 9 per axis;
$\sum_q w_q=\sqrt\pi$ per axis) gives the **corrected NORMATIVE discrete
formula**:

$$
\boxed{\;
\bigl(F_A(\tau) f\bigr)_k \;=\; e^{\tau c(x_k)} \cdot \frac{1}{\pi^{D/2}}
\sum_{q_1, \ldots, q_D} w_{q_1} \cdots w_{q_D}\,
f\!\bigl(x_k + \tau\, b(x_k) + 2\sqrt{\tau}\,\sigma_{A(x_k)}\,\eta_q\bigr)
\;}
\tag{32.3}
$$

where $\eta_q = (\eta_{q_1}, \ldots, \eta_{q_D})$ are the tensor Gauss-Hermite
nodes, $w_{q_i}$ the per-axis weights, and $\sigma_{A(x_k)}$ the Cholesky factor
of $A(x_k)$ ($A(x_k)=\sigma\sigma^T$, computed once at construction and cached).

**The three corrections versus the pre-v6 form** (each independently required):
1. **Normalisation $\pi^{-D/2}$** — equivalently divide the per-axis weights by
   $\sqrt\pi$. Restores $F_A(0)=I$ exactly: at $\tau=0$ the shift vanishes and
   $\pi^{-D/2}\sum_q w_q\, f(x_k) = \pi^{-D/2}\cdot\pi^{D/2}\, f(x_k) = f(x_k)$.
2. **Node scale $2\sqrt\tau$** — the whitening substitution forces
   $(2\sqrt\tau\, s)^2/(4\tau)=s^2$; the pre-v6 $\sqrt{2\tau}$ scale put the
   Gaussian variance off by a factor of 2 (it produced heat variance
   $\tau\,A$ instead of the correct $2\tau\,A$).
3. **No $1/\sqrt{\det A}$ residual** — the $\sqrt{\det A}$ of (32.1) is exactly
   cancelled by the Jacobian $\det\sigma=\sqrt{\det A}$ of the whitening
   substitution; the implementation must NOT carry a separate $\det A$ factor
   (it is absorbed by using $\sigma$ as the node-transport matrix). This is why
   (32.3) shows neither $\det A$ nor $(4\pi\tau)^{D/2}$ — both are subsumed.

**$F(0)=I$ unit witness (NORMATIVE).** For $f\equiv 1$, $c\equiv 0$, any $A$,
any $\tau\ge 0$: $\bigl(F_A(\tau)\,1\bigr)_k = \pi^{-D/2}\sum_q w_q = 1$. This is
a REQUIRED smoke sub-test of the G_DDIM gate (see §32.5): the kernel applied to
the constant function must return the constant function to machine precision for
$D\in\{1,2,3,4,5\}$ and a sweep of $\tau$.

**Validation of (32.3) against the v0.1.0 1D case**: when $D = 1$,
$a_{11}(x) = a(x)$, $b_1(x) = b(x)$, equation (32.3) is the 5-point
Gauss-Hermite quadrature of the SAME continuous Gaussian average that the §1
formula (6) discretises with the closed-form $\{\tfrac14,\tfrac14,\tfrac12\}$
3-point rule. The two are NOT byte-identical (different quadrature rules of the
same integral); the pre-v6 "byte-identity sub-test of G_DDIM at $D=1$" claim was
**incorrect** and is RETRACTED (ADR-0112). The agreement is to quadrature
accuracy ($O(10^{-9})$ on the smooth Gaussian test datum), not bit-for-bit. The
correct $D=1$ sanity sub-test is the $F(0)=I$ unit witness above plus
convergence agreement of $(F_A(\tau/n))^n$ to the 1D `ShiftChernoff1D` result
within the order-1 self-convergence band.

### §32.5 — Acceptance gate G_DDIM (NORMATIVE library)

> **v6.0.0 CORRECTION (ADR-0112).** Two normative changes from the pre-v6 spec:
> (1) the order claim is corrected from **order-2** to **order-1** — the frozen
> coefficient kernel (32.3) is genuinely order-1 for variable $A(x)$ (sympy +
> empirical proof in ADR-0112); the claimed "ζ²-d-D correction baked into the
> baseline" never existed in the implementation. The gate threshold is therefore
> $\le -0.95$ (the standard order-1 precedent, matching G24/G25/G27-base). (2) The
> per-axis grid resolution $N$ is now a $D$-dependent ladder; the uniform
> $N=128$ was physically infeasible for $D\ge 4$ ($128^5\cdot 8 = 274$ GB).
>
> **v6.0.0 AMENDMENT 1 (ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1, 2026-05-30).** The N(D) ladder is
> corrected AGAIN — to a UNIFORM COARSE grid $N_{\text{AXIS}}(D)=\{8,8,8,6\}$,
> $n_{\mathrm{ref}}(D)=512$ for all $D$. An adversarial QA pass empirically
> falsified the original "fine grid is fine because the spatial floor cancels
> common-mode" reasoning: at $D=2,N=128$ the slope is $\approx -0.05$ (floor-
> dominated, FAILS the gate); at $D=2,N=8$ it is $\approx -1.03$ (clean). The
> spatial error here is per-step multilinear INTERPOLATION error at off-grid
> Gauss-Hermite nodes; it accumulates as $O(n\cdot dx^2)$ and does NOT cancel
> between the $n$-step iterate and the $n_{\mathrm{ref}}$-step reference (different
> step counts). A coarse grid is REQUIRED so the temporal-truncation signal
> dominates the interpolation floor. See "Why a COARSE grid is required" below
> and ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1.

**G_DDIM (RELEASE_BLOCKING — d-D anisotropic shift convergence slope, per-D sweeps)**:

**Resolution ladder $N_{\text{AXIS}}(D)$ / $n_{\mathrm{ref}}(D)$ (NORMATIVE — coarse grid required; ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1).**
The grid is deliberately COARSE. The dominant spatial error is per-step multilinear
INTERPOLATION error of `GridFnND::sample` at off-grid Gauss-Hermite shifted points;
it accumulates as $O(n\cdot dx^2)$ along each trajectory and does NOT cancel between
the $n$-step iterate and the $n_{\mathrm{ref}}$-step reference. A FINE grid drives
this interpolation floor below the genuine $O(1/n)$ temporal-truncation signal at the
WRONG step-count scaling, flattening the measured slope toward 0; a COARSE grid
inflates $dx^2$ so the temporal-truncation signal dominates. The gated tests use:

| $D$ | $N_{\text{AXIS}}(D)$ | grid nodes $N^D$ | grid mem ($\times 8$ B) | $5^D$ quad/pt | $n_{\mathrm{ref}}(D)$ | $n$-sweep | gate (slope $\le$) |
|----|------|------------------|-------------------------|---------------|-----------------------|-----------|--------------------|
| 2  | 8    | 64               | 0.5 KB                  | 25            | 512                   | $\{32,64,128,256\}$ | $-0.95$ |
| 3  | 8    | 512              | 4 KB                    | 125           | 512                   | $\{32,64,128,256\}$ | $-0.95$ |
| 4  | 8    | 4 096            | 33 KB                   | 625           | 512                   | $\{16,32,64,128\}$  | $-0.95$ |
| 5  | 6    | 7 776            | 62 KB                   | 3 125         | 512                   | $\{16,32,64,128\}$  | $-0.95$ |

Rationale: $N_{\text{AXIS}}(D)=\{8,8,8,6\}$ is chosen COARSE so that grid spacing
$dx\approx 1.43$ (D≤4) is comparable to the 5-point Gauss-Hermite node displacement,
keeping the temporal-truncation signal above the interpolation floor across the
sweep. $n_{\mathrm{ref}}(D)=512$ uniformly for ALL $D$ (a $\ge 2\times$ separation
from the coarsest sweep point: $n=256$ for $D=2,3$ and $n=128$ for $D=4,5$). At
$D=5$ the curse of dimensionality forces $N_{\text{AXIS}}=6$ ($6^5\cdot 5^5$ is the
CI-budget edge); see the D=5 thin-margin note below.

> **The pre-AMENDMENT-1 ladder $\{128,32,8,6\}$ with $n_{\mathrm{ref}}=\{2048,2048,512,512\}$
> was WRONG for $D=2,3$.** It was justified by a "spatial floor cancels common-mode"
> argument (an untested analogy to the v2.2 `G_NS2D_aniso` finite-difference gate).
> An adversarial QA pass (2026-05-30) measured $D=2,N=128\Rightarrow$ slope $\approx -0.05$
> (FAILS) and $D=3,N=32\Rightarrow$ slope $\approx -0.67$ (FAILS), versus clean
> $\approx -1.03 / -1.20$ at $N=8$. The analogy failed because the FD Laplacian's
> spatial error is step-count-independent (genuinely common-mode) whereas this
> kernel's interpolation error scales with step count. See ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1.

Setup (per dimension $D \in \{2, 3, 4, 5\}$):
```
let N = N_AXIS[D];                                               // {2:8, 3:8, 4:8, 5:6} — coarse (ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1)
let grid: GridND<f64, D> = GridND::new([-5.0; D], [5.0; D], [N; D])?;

// Anisotropic diffusion tensor: identity + small off-diagonal coupling.
let a_ij = |x: &[f64; D]| -> SquareMatrix<f64, D> {
    let mut a = SquareMatrix::<f64, D>::identity();
    for i in 0..D {
        for j in (i+1)..D {
            a[(i, j)] = 0.25 * (x[i] + x[j]).tanh();             // smooth bounded off-diagonal
            a[(j, i)] = a[(i, j)];
        }
    }
    a
};
let b_i = |_x: &[f64; D]| -> [f64; D] { [0.0; D] };              // no drift
let c   = |_x: &[f64; D]| -> f64        { 0.0 };                  // no reaction

let kernel = AnisotropicShiftChernoffND::<f64, D>::new(
    a_ij, b_i, c, grid.clone(),
)?;

// Witness — verify Theorem 32.1 prerequisites hold on test data.
let f0 = GridFnND::<f64, D>::from_fn(&grid, |x| (-x.iter().map(|xi| xi*xi).sum::<f64>()).exp());
assert!(kernel.in_subspace::<2>(&f0));                            // C²_b core; via v3.0 B1
```

Sweep: $n \in \{32, 64, 128, 256\}$ (for $D\in\{2,3\}$) or $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$
(for $D\in\{4,5\}$) at fixed $T = 0.5$ (so $\tau = T / n$).

Reference solution: high-resolution `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND` at $n_{\mathrm{ref}}(D)=512$ on the SAME grid (self-convergence gate). The high-resolution result is the de-facto reference because the closed-form analytical fundamental solution is available only for constant $A$ (constant-coefficient anisotropic Gaussian); for the variable-$A$ test datum, the high-resolution Chernoff iterate is the only available reference.

Per-dimension gate (the SAME threshold for ALL $D\in\{2,3,4,5\}$):
```
err_n := ||F^n(f₀) - u_ref||_∞;
slope := OLS_log_log(err_n vs 1/n) over the per-D n-sweep above;
ASSERT slope.is_finite() && slope <= -0.95;       // order-1; NaN/Inf is a HARD FAIL
```

**Why a COARSE grid is required (NOT "N-robust" — ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 1).** The
sweep iterate and $u_{\mathrm{ref}}$ are built from the SAME kernel on the SAME grid,
but their spatial errors are NOT common-mode. The dominant spatial error is the
per-step multilinear interpolation error of `GridFnND::sample` at the off-grid
Gauss-Hermite shifted points $x_k + 2\sqrt{\tau}\,\sigma\,\eta_q$; it accumulates as
$O(n\cdot dx^2)$ per trajectory, and the iterate ($n$ steps) and reference
($n_{\mathrm{ref}}=512$ steps) take a DIFFERENT number of steps, so the accumulated
interpolation floors do NOT cancel in $\|F^n f_0 - u_{\mathrm{ref}}\|$. On a FINE
grid the interpolation floor (small in absolute terms but at a temporal-step-count
scaling) dominates the genuine $O(1/n)$ temporal-truncation signal and flattens the
measured slope toward 0 (empirically: $D=2,N=128\Rightarrow -0.05$;
$D=3,N=32\Rightarrow -0.67$). A COARSE grid inflates $dx^2$ so the
temporal-truncation signal dominates across the sweep, recovering the true order-1
slope ($D=2,N=8\Rightarrow -1.03$; $D=3,N=8\Rightarrow -1.20$). The "exact for
constant $A$" property of (32.3) is a property of the CONTINUOUS formula; the
discretised kernel ALWAYS carries the $O(dx^2)$ interpolation error regardless of $A$.
Hence the gate is N-SENSITIVE and the coarse $N_{\text{AXIS}}(D)=\{8,8,8,6\}$ ladder
is mandatory.

**$D=5$ thin-margin honesty note.** At $D=5$ the curse of dimensionality forces
$N_{\text{AXIS}}=6$ (6⁵=7776 nodes × 5⁵=3125 quad/pt is the CI-budget edge;
$N_{\text{AXIS}}=8$ at $D=5$ is infeasible). The measured slope is $\approx -0.9614$,
clearing the $-0.95$ gate by a THIN margin (~1.5%). Order-1 at $D=5$ is demonstrated,
but plainly with a thin margin — at $N=6$ the coarse-grid temporal signal only just
dominates the interpolation floor. This is the honest curse-of-dimensionality boundary
of the gate; any tightening of the threshold or change to the $D=5$ quadrature MUST
re-measure this margin.

**$F(0)=I$ smoke sub-test (NORMATIVE, REQUIRED).** Before the slope sweep, each
per-$D$ test asserts $\|F_A(\tau)\,\mathbf 1 - \mathbf 1\|_\infty < 10^{-12}$ for
the constant function $\mathbf 1$ at $\tau\in\{0,\,T/16,\,T/128\}$. This is the
direct guard against the §32.4 normalisation defect and would have caught the
pre-v6 divergence immediately.

**Note (order is 1, not 2).** Theorem 32.1 states — and the implementation
realises — an **order-1** Chernoff kernel for variable $A(x)$: the frozen
coefficient quadrature (32.3) reproduces the exact heat semigroup to all orders
for CONSTANT $A$ (the Gaussian average IS the exact solution), but for variable
$A$ the leading mismatch is $\tfrac{\tau^2}{2}\bigl(a\,a''\,f'' + 2a\,a'\,f'''\bigr)$
per step (local error $O(\tau^2)$, global $O(\tau)=O(1/n)$; 1D representative,
proof in ADR-0112). A genuine order-2 lift would require the d-D analog of the
1D ζ-A correction (ADR-0008): explicit gradient/Hessian $\partial_m A(x)$ closures
plus a $\tau^2$ correction polynomial in $A,\partial A,\partial^2 A$ — a major
additive API and a non-trivial derivation (the missing-odd-derivative obstruction
of math.md §9.2.2 reappears in d-D). This is **DEFERRED to a future v4.x/v6.x
`AnisotropicShiftChernoffND` ζ²-d-D variant**; the v6.0.0 baseline ships honest
order-1. `order()` returns `1`.

Per-dimension test files:
- `tests/anisotropic_shift_nd_d2_slope.rs`
- `tests/anisotropic_shift_nd_d3_slope.rs`
- `tests/anisotropic_shift_nd_d4_slope.rs`
- `tests/anisotropic_shift_nd_d5_slope.rs`

All four sub-tests are RELEASE_BLOCKING. The $D = 5$ case is the LARGEST gated dimension — beyond $D = 5$ the kernel compiles but is NOT gated (the tensor-product quadrature cost $5^6 = 15625$ per evaluation point becomes prohibitive for the engineer Wave to run in CI; the v4.x ROADMAP includes a sparse-grid quadrature for $D \ge 6$).

**ApproximationSubspace<2, F> witness**: the v4.0 `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND<F, D>` opts in to `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` per ADR-0073 (the FIFTH v3.x opt-in after the v3.0 trio + v3.1 HypoellipticChernoff). `in_subspace`: returns `true` iff the underlying grid has $\ge 5^D$ points (the tensor-product Gauss-Hermite stencil width) AND the per-axis `BoundaryPolicy` is `Reflect` or `Periodic` (the only stable variants for the d-D shift quadrature).

### §32.6 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **$D \ge 6$ via Smolyak sparse grids**: the tensor-product Gauss-Hermite quadrature $5^D$ is prohibitive for $D \ge 6$. Smolyak sparse grids reduce the cost to $O(D \log^{D-1} q)$ at the price of slightly weaker accuracy bounds. Deferred to v4.1+ — Smolyak quadrature infrastructure is its own engineering surface.
- **Order-2 d-D ζ²-correction (the FIRST deferred lift)**: the v6.0.0 baseline is order-1 (§32.5 Note, ADR-0112). Lifting it to order-2 requires the d-D analog of the 1D ζ-A correction (ADR-0008 / §9.2.3): explicit gradient closures $\partial_m a_{ij}(x)$ (and, for the odd-derivative obstruction, $\partial^2$ terms) plus a $\tau^2$ correction polynomial in $A,\partial A,\partial^2 A$. This is a major additive API + derivation and is DEFERRED to a future v4.x/v6.x variant kernel; the bare order-1 kernel is the v6.0.0 ship. The order-2 lift is the PREREQUISITE for any d-D ζ⁴.
- **Order-4 d-D ζ⁴ correction**: parallel to v3.0 ADR-0075's 1D ζ⁴, a d-D ζ⁴ correction would require the d-D analog of Galkin-Remizov §3.1 — a multi-monomial polynomial in the d-D generator with coefficients depending on $A(x)$ and its derivatives. Deferred indefinitely (it presupposes the order-2 ζ²-d-D lift above, which is itself deferred).
- **Adaptive quadrature with error control**: the v4.0 baseline uses FIXED $q = 5$ Gauss-Hermite per axis. An adaptive quadrature that adjusts $q$ per evaluation point based on a posteriori error estimates defers to v4.x+ (orthogonal track; no current use case demands it).
- **Stochastic d-D shift (Monte Carlo replacement of quadrature)**: as a fallback for $D \ge 5$, replace the quadrature in (32.3) with MC samples. Already part of the `PointEval` Backend E for high-D pointwise eval; the full-grid MC alternative defers to v4.1+ if benchmark evidence supports it.

### §32.7 — References

- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025). — Theorem 3 cousin formula (the d-D anisotropic shift Chernoff; cited for §32.3 Theorem 32.1). The exact wording of Theorem 3 is for the autonomous parabolic generator on $\mathbb{R}^D$; the "cousin" qualifier acknowledges the v0.1.0 1D Theorem 6 specialisation that the library shipped first.
- A. Friedman, *Partial Differential Equations of Parabolic Type*, Prentice-Hall 1964 (reprinted Dover 2008). — §1.4 (the canonical reference for the d-D anisotropic Gaussian fundamental solution; cited for §32.2 equation 32.1).
- v0.1.0 `ShiftChernoff1D` precedent: math.md §1-§2 (the 1D specialisation; the byte-identity sub-test of G_DDIM at $D = 1$ confirms the d-D formula reduces to the 1D verbatim).
- v0.3.0 `DiffusionChernoff` precedent: math.md §9.2.3.B (the ζ-A $\tau^2$-correction for 1D variable-coefficient diffusion; the v4.0 d-D kernel inherits the same correction pattern).
- ADR-0081 (this section's contract authority; references back to §32.1-§32.5 verbatim).

### §32.8 — v7.0.0 PRE-FLIGHT GO notes (NORMATIVE pointer; supersedes the §32.6 "deferred" status of three bullets)

The §32.6 future-extension bullets above are HISTORICAL (v6.0.0 deferral record). v7.0.0 Phase-5 PRE-FLIGHT (2026-06-05) cleared three of them to GO; the §32.6 prose is retained for audit trail and superseded here:

- **Order-2 d-D ζ²-correction → GO (ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 2)**. Sympy PRE-FLIGHT `scripts/verify_anisotropic_shift_zeta2_ddim.py` proves: (i) τ⁰,τ¹ deficit = 0 (frozen kernel is order-1, Theorem 32.1); (ii) **all-constant (A,b) τ²-deficit = 0** (frozen kernel exact for constant coefficients, §32.2 confirmed); (iii) the A-gradient sources a non-trivial τ²-deficit (D=1 → −1249/9800, D=2 → −8129/29400) that an explicit C₂ from $\partial_m a_{ij}$ closures KILLS — the d-D analog of the §9.2.3.B bracket. Shipped as the ADDITIVE constructor `with_zeta2_correction` (`order()` of the base type unchanged). Gate `G_AS_ZETA2_DDIM` (slope ≤ −1.95, COARSE-grid AMENDMENT-1 protocol). **Engineer caveat (PRE-FLIGHT-surfaced):** the §32 frozen kernel freezes A AND b; variable b ALSO sources a τ²-deficit (D=1 → −42121/180075, D=2 → −191783/360150). The ζ² lift corrects the ∂A (diffusion) piece; the §32.5 gate datum has b≡0 so the gate is clean. The ∂b drift-gradient correction is a follow-on (still deferred).

- **Adaptive per-point quadrature q → GO (ADR-0122)**. `scripts/verify_adaptive_quad.py` proves the per-point selector `q* = min{q∈{3,5,7,9} : |I_q−I_{q-2}| ≤ tol}` matches fixed-32 within `≤ 8.98e-13` on the kernel-envelope datum (gate `G_ADAPTIVE_Q`, ≤1e-10) at mean q* = 5.33 vs accuracy-equivalent fixed-9 (41% fewer nodes/axis). **Load-bearing caveat:** the estimator tol MUST default to the production target (1e-10), NOT machine-epsilon, else it over-refines transcendental integrands to q=9 and the saving evaporates.

- **$D \ge 5$ via Smolyak sparse grids → GO (ADR-0123)**. `scripts/verify_smolyak_sparse.py` builds the combination technique $A(\ell,D) = \sum_{\ell-D+1 \le |i| \le \ell} (-1)^{\ell-|i|}\binom{D-1}{\ell-|i|}\bigotimes_k U_{i_k}$ from the in-tree nested GH ladder. At D=5: ℓ=8 → **341 nodes** match the tensor 5⁵=3125 reference to rel 1.15e-6 (**9.2× reduction**); ℓ=7 → 71 nodes nail total-degree-5 (44× reduction). Bakeable as generated in-tree constants — **NO 4th dependency** (constitution Override #1 respected). Gate `G_SMOLYAK_D5` (slope ≤ −0.95 — order-1; the shipped test corrects ADR-0123's stale −1.95 prose since `SmolyakGridND::order() = 1`; nodes < 3125). **Caveat:** Smolyak weights carry SIGNS; the `F(0)=I` unit witness (Σ merged weights = π^{D/2}) must be asserted as a smoke sub-test.

- **$D \ge 6$ via Smolyak sparse grids → IN-SCOPE for v8.0.0 (ADR-0123 AMENDMENT 1, Phase-4 item C1)**. The §32.6 "$D \ge 6$ … deferred to v4.1+" bullet above is SUPERSEDED: D≥6 was deferred ONLY for CI budget, NOT for math. The shipped `SmolyakGridND<F, const D>` and its `build_smolyak<D>` / `enumerate_multi_index<D>` / `add_tensor_product<D>` pipeline are ALREADY fully generic over `const D`; the $D \ge 6$ surface is the SAME type instantiated at $D = 6$, gated by `G_SMOLYAK_D6`. PRE-FLIGHT `scripts/verify_smolyak_sparse.py` D=6 sweep (2026-06-07): at the default $\ell = D + 3 = 9$ the sparse grid is **533 nodes** vs the full tensor $6^6 = 46656$ — an **87.5× reduction**; the unit witness $\sum w = \pi^{D/2} = \pi^3 = 31.00628$ holds to $\le 10^{-13}$ at every level $\ell \in \{6,7,8,9,10\}$ (nodes $\{1,13,97,533,2381\}$). The nested GH ladder depth (max level 5, rules $\{1,3,5,7,9\}$-pt) suffices: the deepest 1-D rule used at $\ell = 9, D = 6$ is level $\ell - D + 1 = 4 \le 5$. **Structural prerequisite (engineer caveat):** `SquareMatrix<F, D>` stores its $D \times D$ flat data in a fixed `[F; 25]` oversized-static (sized for $D \le 5$, since $5 \times 5 = 25$); at $D = 6$, $D \cdot D = 36 > 25$ and `set(i, j)` writes index $i + jD$ up to $5 + 5 \cdot 6 = 35$, out of bounds. The widening `[F; 25] → [F; 36]` (covering $D \le 6$) is the ONLY blocker; it is an internal-storage change (no public-API break — the array length is an implementation detail per the field's own rustdoc "first D*D slots used"). The order-1 reality (slope ≤ −0.95) and the SIGN-carrying weights caveat transfer verbatim from D=5.

- The **order-4 d-D ζ⁴** and **Monte-Carlo full-grid** bullets remain DEFERRED (ζ⁴ presupposes the now-GO ζ² lift landing first; MC awaits benchmark demand).

---

## §33 — Matrix-valued operators (v4.0, ADR-0082, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §33.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v0.1.0 → v3.1 library covers SCALAR-valued state functions: $f : \mathbb{R}^D \to \mathbb{R}$ (or $\mathbb{C}$ at v4.0). For COUPLED-COMPONENT PDE systems where the state is $u : \mathbb{R}^D \to \mathbb{R}^M$ (a vector of $M$ scalar components per spatial point) with each component coupled to the others via the operator $L$, the v2.x library has no native support — users must either (a) hand-encode the coupling via composition of $M$ scalar kernels with off-trait coupling steps, or (b) treat the multi-component state as a single block-vector at the cost of losing the per-component grid structure.

The canonical applications are:
- **Reaction-diffusion systems** with $M$ coupled species: $(u_t)_i = \sum_j D_{ij} \Delta u_j + R_i(u_1, \ldots, u_M)$ where $D_{ij}$ is the cross-diffusion tensor (per Hilhorst-Mimura 1999 §2; the FitzHugh-Nagumo neurone model has $M = 2$, $D_{12} = 0$ in the standard formulation but $D_{12} \ne 0$ in extended formulations).
- **Multi-population kinetic models** with $M$ population types coupled through cross-collision terms.
- **Multi-asset financial PDEs** with $M$ underlying asset types coupled through cross-correlation.
- **Quantum spin systems** with $M$ spin components coupled through Pauli matrices ($M = 2$ for spin-1/2).

v4.0 ADR-0082 ships `MatrixDiffusionChernoff<F, const M: usize>` for the linear coupled-diffusion generator $(L u)_i = \sum_j a_{ij}(x) \partial_x^2 u_j + \sum_j b_{ij}(x) \partial_x u_j + \sum_j c_{ij}(x) u_j$ on $\mathbb{R}$ (1D base) with $u \in \mathbb{R}^M$.

### §33.2 — Coupled-component state type (NORMATIVE library)

**Definition 33.1 (Matrix grid function).** A `MatrixGridFn1D<F, const M: usize>` is a state representation for $u : \mathrm{Grid}_h \to \mathbb{R}^M$ on the 1D discrete grid $\mathrm{Grid}_h$ with $N$ points. Internal layout: row-major `[F; N * M]` with the $i$-th component at grid point $k$ stored at index $k \cdot M + i$. This layout is optimal for the per-grid-point matrix-vector multiply at the heart of the per-step matrix exponential (§33.3 below).

Implements `State<F>` via per-component delegation:
- `axpy(α, &other)`: per-component axpy on each of the $M$ components.
- `scale(α)`: per-component scaling on each of the $M$ components.
- `norm_sup()`: maximum sup-norm across the $M$ components.
- `zeroed_like(other)`: zero matrix-state of the same grid + same $M$.

### §33.3 — Matrix exponential per step (CITATION — Higham 2008 §10 Padé)

**Theorem 33.1 (Coupled-diffusion Chernoff, NORMATIVE library — math.md §33.3).** The matrix-valued Chernoff step is the matrix analog of `DiffusionChernoff`:

$$
\bigl(F_M(\tau) u\bigr)_i(x) \;=\; \sum_j \bigl[\exp\bigl(\tau \cdot C(x)\bigr)\bigr]_{ij} \cdot \bigl[\sum_k (D_h^{-1})_{ij,k} \cdot (a_{kl}(x) u_l)(x)\bigr]
\tag{33.1}
$$

where $C(x) = (c_{ij}(x))_{i,j=1}^M$ is the per-grid-point reaction matrix and $\exp(\tau C(x))$ is the matrix exponential. For $M \le 4$, closed-form Cayley-Hamilton formulas give the matrix exponential in $O(M^3)$ arithmetic operations per grid point per step; for $M \ge 5$, the Padé approximation of Higham 2008 *Functions of Matrices* §10 is used (cost: $O(M^3 \log_2 \|\tau C\|)$ per grid point per step).

**Per-step algorithm (NORMATIVE library)**:

```
MatrixDiffusionChernoff::apply_into(τ, u_src, u_dst, scratch):
  // Step 1 — discrete diffusion: per-component diffusion via tridiagonal LU.
  for i in 0..M:
    for j in 0..M:
      // Apply the (i, j) component of the coupled diffusion operator.
      diffusion_apply(τ, a_ij, b_ij, &u_src[component j], &mut intermediate[component i]);
  // Step 2 — pointwise matrix exponential of reaction matrix:
  for k in 0..N:                                                       // each grid point
    let C_k = reaction_matrix_at(k);                                   // M × M matrix
    let exp_C_k = matrix_exp(τ * C_k);                                  // Cayley-Hamilton or Padé
    let u_k = u_dst.point_view(k);                                      // M-vector
    let intermediate_k = intermediate.point_view(k);                    // M-vector
    matrix_vec_mul(&exp_C_k, &intermediate_k, &mut u_k);                // u_dst[k] = exp(τ C_k) · intermediate[k]
```

The per-step cost is $O(N \cdot M^3)$ for the matrix exponentials plus $O(N \cdot M^2)$ for the diffusion. For $N = 512$ and $M = 4$, the per-step cost is $\approx 512 \cdot 64 + 512 \cdot 16 = 41{,}000$ FLOPs — fast at the per-step level.

### §33.4 — Acceptance gate G_MATRIX (NORMATIVE library)

**G_MATRIX (RELEASE_BLOCKING — coupled-diffusion convergence on $M \in \{2, 3, 4\}$)**:

Setup (per $M$):
```
let N = 128_usize;
let grid = Grid1D::<f64>::new(-5.0, 5.0, N)?;

// Deterministic SPD coupling matrices via canonical PCG64 seed.
let rng = PCG64::new(0xC0FFEE_BABE_DEAD_BEEF);
let a_ij = generate_spd_matrix_field::<M>(&grid, &rng);                // M × M SPD per grid point
let b_ij = generate_skew_matrix_field::<M>(&grid, &rng);               // skew-symmetric drift
let c_ij = generate_symmetric_matrix_field::<M>(&grid, &rng);          // symmetric reaction

let kernel = MatrixDiffusionChernoff::<f64, M>::new(
    a_ij, b_ij, c_ij, grid.clone(),
)?;
```
