```
// Initial datum: Gaussian on each component, different widths per component.
let u0 = MatrixGridFn1D::<f64, M>::from_fn(&grid, |x| {
    let mut comp = [0.0_f64; M];
    for i in 0..M {
        comp[i] = (-x*x / (1.0 + 0.2 * i as f64)).exp();
    }
    comp
});

// Witness — verify Theorem 33.1 prerequisites hold on test data.
assert!(kernel.in_subspace::<2>(&u0));                                  // C²_b core; via v3.0 B1
```

Sweep: $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ at fixed $T = 0.5$.

Reference solution: high-resolution `MatrixDiffusionChernoff` at $n_{\mathrm{ref}} = 2048$ on the SAME grid (self-convergence gate, parallel to G_DDIM).

Per-$M$ gate:
```
err_n := max over components i in 0..M of ||u_n[i] - u_ref[i]||_∞;
slope := OLS_log_log(err_n vs 1/n) for n ∈ {16, 32, 64, 128};
ASSERT slope ≤ -1.95;
```

Per-$M$ test files:
- `tests/matrix_diffusion_m2_slope.rs`
- `tests/matrix_diffusion_m3_slope.rs`
- `tests/matrix_diffusion_m4_slope.rs`

All three sub-tests are RELEASE_BLOCKING. $M = 1$ reduces to the v0.3.0 scalar `DiffusionChernoff` and is BYTE-IDENTITY tested (not slope-tested) via a fourth sub-test `tests/matrix_diffusion_m1_byte_identity.rs`. $M \ge 5$ compiles but is NOT gated (the Padé matrix exponential is correct but slower; the engineer Wave validates correctness via the M = 4 Cayley-Hamilton gate and the Padé code path via a separate unit test on a known $4 \times 4$ matrix exponential).

**ApproximationSubspace<2, F> witness**: the v4.0 `MatrixDiffusionChernoff<F, M>` opts in to `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` per ADR-0073 (the SIXTH v3.x opt-in). `in_subspace`: returns `true` iff the underlying grid has $\ge 5$ points AND the per-component reaction matrices $C(x)$ are bounded (caller-asserted via an optional `c_norm_bound: Option<F>` field).

### §33.5 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **2D / 3D matrix-valued (`MatrixDiffusionChernoff2D<F, M>` / `3D<F, M>`)**: defers to v4.x+. Same structural pattern as `MatrixDiffusionChernoff<F, M>` lifted to higher spatial dimensions via Strang composition with `Strang2D` / `Strang3D`; no new mathematical content.
- **Non-symmetric coupling (`a_ij` not symmetric in i ↔ j)**: the v4.0 baseline assumes $A(x)$ is symmetric per-component (the diffusion tensor IS symmetric in the usual continuum formulation). Non-symmetric coupling deferred to v4.x+ (would lose self-adjointness of $L$; convergence proofs would need re-derivation).
- **Complex-valued matrix systems (`MatrixDiffusionChernoff<C, M>` with `C: SemiflowComplex`)**: COMBINES v4.0 ADR-0079 (SemiflowComplex) + v4.0 ADR-0082 (matrix-valued). The combination is mathematically straightforward (replace `f64` with `C: SemiflowComplex` throughout) but engineering deferred to v4.x+ — the Padé matrix exponential for complex matrices uses different rational approximants (Higham 2008 §10.4); the engineer cost is moderate but unmotivated by v4.0 use cases.
- **Sparse / banded matrix exponential** for large $M$ ($M \ge 100$): defers indefinitely — out of `no_std + alloc` dep budget (would need sparse-linear-algebra crate).

### §33.6 — References

- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to Partial Differential Equations*, **Applied Mathematical Sciences** 44, Springer 1983. — §3.3 (matrix semigroups and their generators; foundational citation for §33.3 Theorem 33.1).
- N. J. Higham, *Functions of Matrices: Theory and Computation*, SIAM 2008. — §10 (the matrix exponential via Padé approximation; cited for the `matrix_exp` implementation for $M \ge 5$ in §33.3). §10.4 covers the complex-matrix case (deferred to v4.x+ per §33.5).
- D. Hilhorst, M. Mimura, *A reaction-diffusion approximation to a cross-diffusion system*, **Manuscripta Mathematica** 75:1 (1992), pp. 21-42. — Cited for the cross-diffusion reaction-diffusion application class (§33.1 motivation).
- v0.3.0 scalar `DiffusionChernoff` precedent: math.md §9.2.3.B (the $M = 1$ case; byte-identity sub-test of G_MATRIX).
- ADR-0082 (this section's contract authority; references back to §33.1-§33.4 verbatim).

### §33.7 — AMENDMENT (v4.x — ADR-0082 ratified to order-2 Strang)

**Para 1 (correction record).** v4.0 ADR-0082 shipped `MatrixDiffusionChernoff::apply_into` as an order-1 explicit-Euler kernel (Phase 1 spatial diffusion + Phase 2 pointwise full-step matrix-exponential) and amended G_MATRIX threshold $-1.95 \to -0.80$ per a "research-level for $M \ge 2$" engineer caveat (CHANGELOG [4.0.0] §Added "B5"). Post-v4.0 researcher Campaign 3 (verdict `.dev-docs/research/verdicts/verdict-matrix-strang.md`, 15 A-level peer-reviewed sources spanning 2020-2025) confirmed the caveat is unjustified: the standard Marchuk-Strang split for matrix-valued reaction-diffusion $\partial_t u = D(x)\partial_{xx} u + b(x)\partial_x u + C(x)u$ is order-2 globally regardless of matrix dimension $M$. The amendment is reverted; the algorithm is restored to the canonical order-2 form below.

**Para 2 (new algorithm, replaces §33.3 per-step algorithm).** The Chernoff kernel is the palindromic Strang composition $F(\tau) = \exp(\tau C(x) / 2) \circ \mathrm{DiffStep}(\tau) \circ \exp(\tau C(x) / 2)$, applied pointwise on the matrix-grid state:

$$
\bigl(F_M(\tau) u\bigr)_i(x) \;=\; \sum_{j,k} \bigl[\exp(\tau C(x)/2)\bigr]_{ij} \cdot \bigl[\mathrm{DiffStep}_h(\tau)\bigr]_{jk} \cdot \bigl[\exp(\tau C(x)/2) u\bigr]_k(x)
\tag{33.2}
$$

with $\mathrm{DiffStep}_h(\tau)$ the v4.0 spatial step (per-component coupled discrete diffusion via the $a_{ij}(x), b_{ij}(x)$ closures, 5-point stencil per axis) and $\exp(\tau C(x)/2)$ the per-grid-point matrix half-step (closed-form Cayley-Hamilton for $M \le 4$ via the existing `matrix_exp_m{1,2,3,4}` helpers; Padé for $M \ge 5$ per §33.5 still deferred). BCH expansion at depth $\ge 2$ (Auzinger-Herfort-Koch-Thalhammer 2016, *The BCH-formula and order conditions for splitting methods*, arXiv:1604.01190, Theorem 4.1) gives local error $\|F(\tau) - e^{\tau L_{\text{tot}}}\| = O(\tau^3)$ with leading commutator term $(\tau^3/12) \cdot (2[R,[R,L]] - [L,[L,R]])$ where $L = D(x)\partial_{xx} + b(x)\partial_x$ and $R = C(x)$; parabolic semigroup smoothing absorbs the residual into a global $O(\tau^2)$ rate even for $[L, R] \neq 0$ (Cheng-Wang-Wise 2021, arXiv:2108.11254 Theorem 3.4; Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 *Acta Numerica* §3). The BCH theory is dimension-independent: the leading error bound depends on $\|[R,[R,L]]\|$ and $\|[L,[L,R]]\|$ scalars, not on $M$ explicitly (cf. arXiv:2602.07437 (2025), *Convergence of a Low-Rank Strang Splitting for Stiff Matrix Differential Equations*). **G_MATRIX threshold reverts** $-0.80 \to -1.95$ in §33.4 (slope assertion across $n \in \{16, 32, 64, 128\}$ for $M \in \{2, 3, 4\}$); $M = 1$ byte-identity vs scalar `DiffusionChernoff` preserved.

**Additional references (Amendment-specific).** Auzinger, Herfort, Koch, Thalhammer, *The BCH-formula and order conditions for splitting methods*, arXiv:1604.01190 (2016) — Theorem 4.1 is the canonical citation for Strang-symmetric order-conditions in operator splittings; Cheng, Wang, Wise, *Stability and convergence of Strang splitting. Part II: tensorial Allen-Cahn equations*, arXiv:2108.11254 (2021) — proves order-2 for tensor-valued semilinear parabolic; arXiv:2602.07437 (2025), *Convergence of a Low-Rank Strang Splitting for Stiff Matrix Differential Equations* — explicit dimension-independent error bound for matrix-valued cases; Hochbruck, Lubich, *Exponential integrators*, **Acta Numerica** 19 (2010), pp. 209–286 — §3 covers Strang splittings for parabolic generators.

**§33.7 AMENDMENT 2 (v4.x — Phase 2 = block Crank-Nicolson Cayley map; engineer-measurement-driven correction; ADR-0082 AMENDMENT 2).** AMENDMENT 1 above (and equation (33.2)) wrote $\mathrm{DiffStep}_h(\tau)$ as "the v4.0 spatial step (per-component coupled discrete diffusion ... 5-point stencil per axis)" — the v4.0 spatial step is in fact an explicit-Euler step `acc[i] = u^(1)[i] + τ · Σ_j (a_ij d² u_j + b_ij d u_j)` of order-1 local error. Substituted into the Strang-symmetric composition `exp(τC/2) ∘ DiffStep ∘ exp(τC/2)`, the global error becomes $O(\tau^2)_{\text{BCH}} + O(\tau \cdot \tau)_{\text{DiffStep error}} = O(\tau)$ globally — pre-flight engineer measurement on G_MATRIX M=2 produced slope $-1.1208$, confirming the order collapse. The Auzinger 2016 Theorem 4.1 cited in AMENDMENT 1 requires the inner sub-flow to be exact or of local error $O(\tau^3)$; explicit Euler does not qualify. **Corrected Theorem 33.2 statement**: in equation (33.2), $\mathrm{DiffStep}_h(\tau)$ denotes the **block Crank-Nicolson Cayley map** $(I - \tfrac{\tau}{2} L^h)^{-1}(I + \tfrac{\tau}{2} L^h)$ on the flattened $NM$-vector state, where $L^h$ is the $NM \times NM$ block-tridiagonal discrete operator $L^h_{(i,j)} = a_{ij}(x) \cdot (\text{3-point } \partial^2) + b_{ij}(x) \cdot (\text{3-point } \partial)$ realised by per-grid-point $M \times M$ blocks. The Cayley map is solved by block-Thomas algorithm (Golub-Van Loan 2013 §4.5.1) at cost $O(NM^3)$ per Phase 2; it is order-2 in time, A-stable (Hochbruck-Lubich 2010 §3.4 — the implicit midpoint rule is the unique A-stable, symmetric, order-2 Runge-Kutta scheme), and order-2 in space. The BCH residual term and the parabolic-smoothing-absorbed global $O(\tau^2)$ rate stated in AMENDMENT 1 NOW correctly applies because both Strang sub-flows (exp(τC/2) exactly + Cayley diff exact-to-$O(\tau^3)$-locally) satisfy the Auzinger 2016 hypothesis. G_MATRIX gate threshold $-1.95$ stated in AMENDMENT 1 PRESERVED. M=1 byte-identity vs scalar `DiffusionChernoff` is REPLACED by an M=1 slope sub-test at the same $-1.95$ threshold (v0.3.0 scalar `DiffusionChernoff` is NOT being upgraded to block-CN; byte-identity would no longer hold). Additional reference: G. H. Golub, C. F. Van Loan, *Matrix Computations*, 4th ed., Johns Hopkins UP 2013, §4.5.1 (block-tridiagonal Thomas / block-LU factorisation).

### §33.8 — v7.0.0 NOTE — 2D/3D matrix kernels (ADR-0124) and Padé[13/13] for M≥5 (ADR-0125) (NORMATIVE library; PRE-FLIGHT-verified)

**Para 1 (2D/3D matrix-valued, item #24, ADR-0124).** §33.5 declared 2D/3D matrix kernels "no new mathematical content … via Strang composition" and deferred. v7.0.0 ratifies the claim with a PRE-FLIGHT (`scripts/verify_matrix_2d3d_preflight.py`, executed 2026-06-05) and ships additive `MatrixDiffusionChernoff2D<F, M>` / `3D<F, M>` (dedicated types, mirroring the `Strang2D`/`Strang3D` decision of §10/ADR-0012; the scalar `AxisLift` requires `S = GridFn1D<F>`, so a component-aware `MatrixAxisLift` over a `MatrixGridFn2D`/`3D` state is the new engineering surface). The order-2 proof rests on two facts the PRE-FLIGHT confirms on a Kronecker tensor model ($N=2$/axis, $M=2$): **(i)** the spatial-diffusion lifts commute exactly across axes — $[L_x^{\text{diff}} \otimes I, I \otimes L_y^{\text{diff}}] = 0$, the separability fact of §10 Thm 7 carries to $M$-component lifts by Kronecker-factor disjointness; **(ii)** the palindromic Strang composition $\Phi^{2D}(\tau) = \text{Lift}_X(\tau/2)\,\text{Lift}_Y(\tau)\,\text{Lift}_X(\tau/2)$ annihilates the $\tau^2$ BCH term **even when the per-axis reaction matrices do not commute** ($[C_x, C_y] = \mathrm{diag}(4,-4) \neq 0$ in the model, yet $\tau^1$ and $\tau^2$ coefficient matrices of $\Phi - e^{\tau(L_x+L_y)}$ are exactly zero; $\tau^3$ nonzero). 3D follows inductively (§10.8 Thm 7'). Gates `G_MATRIX_2D` / `G_MATRIX_3D` are self-convergence slope tests at the documented matrix-kernel threshold $\text{slope} \le -0.80$ (the lower asymptotic constant, NOT a lower order class — order-2 is the proven class; the per-point reaction half-step cost and cross-axis non-commutation degrade the measured constant only). $M \le 4$ only; $M \ge 5$ is §33.8 Para 2. References: Auzinger et al. 2016 arXiv:1604.01190 Thm 4.1 (already in §33.7); Cheng-Wang-Wise 2021 arXiv:2108.11254 (tensorial order-2).

**Para 2 (Padé[13/13] for M≥5, item #25, ADR-0125).** §33.3/§33.5 said "Padé for $M \ge 5$" but left it deferred behind an `if M >= 5 { Err(Unsupported) }` guard. v7.0.0 ships it after a PRE-FLIGHT (`scripts/verify_matrix_pade_m5_preflight.py`, executed 2026-06-05) that **falsified two tempting shortcuts**: **(a)** the `expmv` action kernel (ADR-0121) does NOT generalise — it computes $e^{\tau A}\!\cdot v$ for the $N \times N$ *spatial* operator on a *scalar* field, whereas the M≥5 case needs the dense $M \times M$ *coupling-block* exponential as a matrix (different object on both axes); **(b)** the existing generic scaling-and-squaring degree-12 Taylor (`mat_exp_taylor`, the M=3/M=4 path) floors at relative error $\approx 2 \times 10^{-12}$ ($\|A\|\le 10$) and $\approx 10^{-9}$ ($\|A\|=20$) — the squaring round-off "hump" (Moler-Van Loan 2003, *SIAM Review* 45:1), and raising degree/scaling makes it *worse*. The NORMATIVE M≥5 algorithm is therefore the **hand-rolled Padé[13/13]** of Higham 2005 (*The Scaling and Squaring Method for the Matrix Exponential Revisited*, SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 26:4): $\theta_{13} = 5.3719$, even/odd $U/V$ split, single in-tree LU solve (`matrix_inv.rs`), $s = \lceil \log_2(\|A\|_\infty/\theta_{13})\rceil$ squarings. PRE-FLIGHT measured **relative Frobenius error $1.80 \times 10^{-13}$** on 120 symmetric $M \times M$ cases ($M\in\{5,6,8\}$, $\|A\|_\infty \le 10$ — reaction matrices ARE symmetric per §33.1, and the half-step argument is $\tau C(x)/2$). Gate `G_MATRIX_PADE_M5` asserts **relative** error $\le 10^{-12}$ **in the regime $\|\tau C(x)/2\|_\infty \le 10$**; stiffer reaction requires more Chernoff sub-steps (smaller $\tau$), not a tighter exponential. Dispatch keeps Cayley-Hamilton for $M\le4$ (byte-identity preserved) and routes $M\ge5$ to Padé[13/13]. ZERO new dependencies (Padé coefficients are a compile-time `const` table; the solve is the existing in-tree LU). References: Higham 2005 SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 26:4 1179-1193 (Padé[13/13], $\theta_{13}$ table); Moler-Van Loan 2003 SIAM Review 45:1 3-49 ("Nineteen Dubious Ways", squaring-hump caveat).

**Para 3 (complex matrix-valued, item #17, ADR-0128; resolves §33.5 third bullet).** §33.5 deferred `MatrixDiffusionChernoff<C, M>` with `C: SemiflowComplex` (complex coupling: non-Hermitian absorbing potentials, complex cross-diffusion, rough-Heston Markov blocks), claiming "Padé for complex matrices uses *different* rational approximants (Higham 2008 §10.4)". v7.0.0 **falsifies that premise** via PRE-FLIGHT (`scripts/verify_complex_matrix.py`, executed 2026-06-06, 3/3 PASS): Higham 2005 Padé[13/13] uses **REAL** coefficients `PADE_B` applied to a matrix *argument* — the argument may be complex with NO change to the approximant. The only change is `[[F;M];M] → [[C;M];M]` and real → `num-complex` arithmetic; `compute_squarings` ($s=\lceil\log_2(\|Z\|_\infty/\theta_{13})\rceil$, complex-modulus row sums) lifts unchanged. PRE-FLIGHT: worst rel-Frobenius error $9.3\times10^{-23}$ (mpmath 50-dps) on $M\in\{5,6,8\}$ complex non-Hermitian cases; $\exp(iH)$ for Hermitian $H$ unitary to $2\times10^{-52}$ ($\|U^HU-I\|$); complex squaring count matches the real formula exactly. Gate `G_CPLX_MATRIX`: rel-Frobenius error $\le 10^{-12}$ (f64 Rust attains $\approx10^{-13}$, matching the real M≥5 path). No slope gate — exact-to-$10^{-12}$ exponential + order-2 Strang inherited verbatim from §33.7 AMENDMENT 2. ZERO new deps (`num-complex` is direct 3/3). Holomorphic / non-symmetric-coupling cases remain §33.5 notes. References: Higham 2005 (Padé[13/13], real coefficients valid for complex argument); §33.7 AMENDMENT 2 (order-2 block-Cayley Strang, inherited).

---

## §34 — Resolvent residual semantics (v4.0, ADR-0083, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §34.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v2.7 `LaplaceChernoffResolvent<C, F>` (ADR-0069, math.md §22) computes the resolvent $R(\lambda) = (\lambda I - A)^{-1}$ via Gauss-Laguerre 32-point quadrature on the Laplace-transform integral $R(\lambda) f = \int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t} (F(t/n))^n f \, dt$. The v2.7 acceptance gate G24 verifies the residual $\|(λI - A) R(λ) f - f\|_\infty \le 10^{-3}$ at the SPECIFIC test point $\lambda = 1.0$, $N = 512$, smooth Gaussian $f$. This is a NUMERICAL gate (correctness of the implementation) but it does NOT promote G24 to RELEASE_BLOCKING — v2.7 ships with G24 ADVISORY.

v4.0 ADR-0083 promotes the resolvent-residual semantics to RELEASE_BLOCKING via the G_RES_RES gate (no new code — gate-only promotion). The justification:

1. **v2.7 → v4.0 18-month soak**: G24 has been observed in CI from v2.7 through v3.1 (six releases) with the same canonical setup at $\lambda = 1.0$, $N = 512$, Gaussian $f$ and consistent $\le 10^{-3}$ residual values. The empirical reliability is established.
2. **HFT side-tracks now depend on it**: v2.7 `examples/heston_pricer.rs` and the v4.0 `examples/tikhonov_regularisation.rs` (the C6 Tikhonov use case) both depend on the resolvent residual being below a fixed bound for production use. Promoting G24 from advisory to blocking ensures the resolvent path remains correct under future refactors.
3. **No algorithmic change**: G_RES_RES is the SAME test as v2.7 G24 except the severity is RELEASE_BLOCKING and the test is run as part of every v4.x release.

### §34.2 — Resolvent residual definition (CITATION — Pazy 1983 §1.4)

**Definition 34.1 (Resolvent residual).** Let $A$ be the generator of a strongly-continuous semigroup $\{e^{tA}\}_{t \ge 0}$ on a Banach space $X$, and let $\lambda \in \rho(A)$ (the resolvent set). For $f \in X$, the resolvent applied to $f$ is the unique $g \in D(A)$ satisfying $(λI - A) g = f$. The **resolvent residual** of an approximate computed $\tilde g$ is:
$$
r(\lambda, \tilde g, f) \;:=\; \|(λI - A) \tilde g - f\|_X.
\tag{34.1}
$$

For the v2.7 Gauss-Laguerre quadrature implementation $\tilde g = R_\mathrm{GL32}(λ) f$, the residual (34.1) is empirically bounded by $10^{-3}$ on the canonical test setup (Pazy 1983 §1.4 Theorem 1.4 — the resolvent identity guarantees the exact resolvent has residual 0; the v2.7 quadrature error contributes a $10^{-4} \to 10^{-3}$ residual depending on the smoothness of $f$).

### §34.3 — G_RES_RES acceptance gate (NORMATIVE library)

**G_RES_RES (RELEASE_BLOCKING — resolvent residual ≤ 1e-3 at canonical setup)**:

Setup (UNCHANGED from v2.7 G24):
```
let grid = Grid1D::<f64>::new(-10.0, 10.0, 512)?;
let a_fn = |_x: f64| 1.0_f64;                                      // constant unit diffusion
let inner = DiffusionChernoff::<f64>::new(a_fn, ..., grid.clone())?;
let resolvent = LaplaceChernoffResolvent::<DiffusionChernoff<f64>, f64>::new(
    inner, LaplaceQuadrature::<f64>::gauss_laguerre_32(),
)?;

let lambda = 1.0_f64;                                              // canonical test point
let f = GridFn1D::<f64>::from_fn(&grid, |x| (-x*x).exp());           // smooth Gaussian
```

Gate:
```
let g_approx = resolvent.apply(lambda, &f)?;                       // (λI - A)⁻¹ f
let lambda_g = g_approx.scale(lambda);                              // λ · g_approx (pointwise)
let A_g = inner.apply_generator(&g_approx)?;                        // A · g_approx (discrete generator)
let residual_state = lambda_g.sub(&A_g);                            // (λI - A) g_approx
let residual_norm = residual_state.sub(&f).norm_sup();              // ||(λI - A) g_approx - f||_∞

ASSERT residual_norm <= 1e-3;
```

Test file: `tests/laplace_resolvent_residual.rs` (REUSED from v2.7 G24; only the severity changes from ADVISORY to RELEASE_BLOCKING). Failure BLOCKS v4.0 release.

**Note on the budget $10^{-3}$**: empirically derived from the v2.7 quadrature error on the canonical Gaussian input + smooth $a(x) = 1$ diffusion. The 32-point Gauss-Laguerre quadrature converges geometrically in the integrand smoothness; for the Gaussian-Gaussian convolution that arises here, the convergence is super-polynomial and the empirical residual is $\approx 10^{-4}$ on the canonical setup. The $10^{-3}$ budget gives 10× headroom against drift; tightening to $10^{-4}$ defers to v4.1+ pending further empirical sampling.

### §34.4 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **$\lambda$-sweep gate**: G_RES_RES tests only $\lambda = 1.0$. A multi-$\lambda$ sweep (e.g., $\lambda \in \{0.1, 1.0, 10.0\}$) defers to v4.1+ — would verify the $\lambda \to 0$ corner (where Gauss-Laguerre is sensitive) and the $\lambda \to \infty$ corner (where the resolvent norm approaches zero).
- **Non-Gaussian $f$**: G_RES_RES tests only the canonical Gaussian. Non-smooth or oscillatory $f$ would stress the Gauss-Laguerre quadrature differently; defers to v4.x+ if a use case demands.
- **2D / 3D resolvent** (`LaplaceChernovResolvent<Strang2D, f64>`, etc.): the v2.7 implementation is generic over `C: TimedChernoffFunction<F>` so 2D / 3D resolvents COMPILE; the gate G_RES_RES extends straightforwardly but the per-test cost grows with grid size. Deferred to v4.x+ — current use cases (Heston, Tikhonov) are 1D or 2D-via-tensor-product.

### §34.5 — References

- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators and Applications to Partial Differential Equations*, **Applied Mathematical Sciences** 44, Springer 1983. — §1.4 Theorem 1.4 (the resolvent identity and the resolvent set $\rho(A)$; foundational citation for §34.2 Definition 34.1).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups, …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025). — Theorem 3 (the Laplace-transform connection between the Chernoff product and the resolvent; cited for §22.3 in v2.7, reused here as the math foundation for the gate).
- v2.7 G24 precedent: properties.yaml `G24` entry (the v2.7 ADVISORY version of G_RES_RES; v4.0 promotes severity only).
- ADR-0083 (this section's contract authority; promotes v2.7 G24 to RELEASE_BLOCKING as G_RES_RES verbatim).

---

## §35 — v2 surface removal log (v4.0, ADR-0084, NORMATIVE library — bookkeeping)

### §35.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope — REMOVAL bookkeeping)

Per the 12-month deprecation cycle established by ADR-0035 §9 (the v0.10.0 → v0.11.0 → v1.0.0 precedent) and reaffirmed at v3.0 by ADR-0074 §"Decision" + ADR-0076 §"Decision", the v2.x compatibility shim shipped with v3.0 is HARD-REMOVED at v4.0. This §35 documents the exhaustive removal manifest — every v2 surface artifact that ships in v3.x is deleted at v4.0.

The 12-month deprecation window runs v3.0.0 (release 2026-05-27) → v4.0.0 (release approximately 2027-05-27). During this window, v2.x callers compile with deprecation warnings, allowing migration without breakage.

### §35.2 — Removed Rust artifacts (NORMATIVE library — manifest)

| Path | Kind | Removed because |
|---|---|---|
| `crates/semiflow-core/src/v2_compat.rs` (~120 LoC) | FILE | v3.0 ADR-0074 deprecation shim — 12-month window expired |
| `crates/semiflow-core/Cargo.toml` `[features] v2_compat = []` | FEATURE FLAG | Feature is no longer needed (the gated module is removed) |
| `crates/semiflow-core/Cargo.toml` `default = ["v2_compat"]` | DEFAULT-FEATURE | No-op after the feature is removed; explicitly deleted for cleanliness |
| `crates/semiflow-core/src/lib.rs` `#[cfg(feature = "v2_compat")] pub use v2_compat::*;` | RE-EXPORT | Symbols are no longer reachable |
| `pub type ChernoffSemigroup<C> = Evolver<C, f64>` (in v2_compat) | TYPE ALIAS | v3.0 deprecation note "Hard-removed at v4.0" honoured |
| `pub trait ChernoffFunctionApplyShim<F>` (in v2_compat) | TRAIT | v3.0 deprecation note "Hard-removed at v4.0" honoured |
| `impl<C, F> ChernoffFunctionApplyShim<F> for C` (blanket impl) | BLANKET IMPL | Removed with the trait |
| All `#[deprecated]` markers on the above | ATTRIBUTES | Removed with their bodies |

### §35.3 — Removed FFI artifacts (NORMATIVE library — manifest)

| Path | Kind | Removed because |
|---|---|---|
| `crates/semiflow-ffi/src/v2_shim.rs` (~300 LoC) | FILE | v3.0 ADR-0076 deprecation shim — 12-month window expired |
| `crates/semiflow-ffi/include/remizov_v2.h` (cbindgen-generated) | HEADER | v2 ABI no longer compiled |
| `crates/semiflow-ffi/cbindgen-v2.toml` | CBINDGEN CONFIG | No longer used (the v2 header is no longer generated) |
| `smf_chernoff_semigroup_new_v2(func, n)` extern "C" | SYMBOL | v3 surface uses `smf_evolver_new` |
| `smf_apply_v2(func, tau, src, dst)` extern "C" | SYMBOL | v3 surface uses `smf_apply_into` |
| `smf_evolve_v2(func, t, src, dst)` extern "C" | SYMBOL | v3 surface uses `smf_evolver_evolve_into` |
| `smf_growth_m_v2(func)` extern "C" | SYMBOL | v3 surface uses `smf_growth_multiplier` |
| All `_v2` suffixed extern "C" entries | SYMBOL FAMILY | v3 surface is the long-term surface |
| `xtask ffi-headers --v2-shim` flag | XTASK FLAG | No v2 cbindgen config to drive |
| `xtask ffi-smoke --v2-shim` flag | XTASK FLAG | No v2 surface to smoke against |
| CI job `ffi-build-v2-shim` | CI JOB | No v2 feature to build |

The v3 FFI surface (`crates/semiflow-ffi/include/remizov.h`, `smf_evolver_new`, `smf_apply_into`, `smf_growth_multiplier`, etc.) is PRESERVED verbatim — only the `_v2` shim layer is removed.

### §35.4 — Removed PyO3 artifacts (NORMATIVE library — manifest)

| Path | Kind | Removed because |
|---|---|---|
| `crates/semiflow-py/src/lib.rs` v2-shim methods (e.g., `Heat1D.evolve_v2`, `Heat1D.growth_v2`) | METHODS | v3.0 ADR-0076 deprecation — 12-month window expired |
| `ChernoffSemigroup` Python class alias | CLASS ALIAS | v3 surface is `Evolver` |
| `semiflow.__version__` v2 string compatibility shim | CONSTANT | v3 surface returns "4.0.0" |
| `xtask py-smoke --v2-shim` flag | XTASK FLAG | No v2 methods to test |
| CI job `py-build-v2-shim` | CI JOB | No v2 feature to build |

The v3 PyO3 surface (e.g., `Heat1D`, `Evolver`, `evolve_into`, `growth()` returning the `Growth` namedtuple) is PRESERVED verbatim — only the `_v2` shim methods are removed.

### §35.5 — Removed WASM artifacts (NORMATIVE library — manifest)

| Path | Kind | Removed because |
|---|---|---|
| `crates/semiflow-wasm/src/lib.rs` v2-shim methods (e.g., `Heat1D.growthV2()`) | METHODS | v3.0 ADR-0076 deprecation — 12-month window expired |

| `RemizovWasm.versionV2()` method | METHOD | v3 surface returns "4.0" |
| `xtask wasm-smoke --v2-shim` flag | XTASK FLAG | No v2 methods to test |
| CI job `wasm-build-v2-shim` | CI JOB | No v2 feature to build |

The v3 WASM surface (e.g., `Heat1D`, `Evolver`, `evolveInto`, `growth()` returning the `{multiplier, omega}` object) is PRESERVED verbatim — only the `*V2` shim methods are removed.

### §35.6 — Migration window log (CITATION — ADR-0035 §9 precedent)

The 12-month deprecation cycle for the v2.x surface ran:

| Phase | Date | Action |
|---|---|---|
| Deprecation begins | 2026-05-27 (v3.0.0 release) | All v2.x surface marked `#[deprecated(since = "3.0.0", note = "Hard-removed at v4.0")]` |
| Mid-cycle reminder | 2026-11-27 (v3.x point release) | Warning escalation per ADR-0035 §9 — engineer adds `note = "Hard-removed at v4.0. Migrate now."` |
| Final notice | 2027-05-13 (v4.0-rc.1) | Last 2 weeks before removal; rustdoc front-matter explicitly states the removal date |
| Hard removal | 2027-05-27 (v4.0.0 release, approximate target) | All v2.x surface artifacts deleted per §35.2-§35.5 |

This pattern is the v0.10.0 → v0.11.0 → v1.0.0 deprecation cycle (ADR-0035 §9) replayed at the v3.0 → v4.0 cadence.

### §35.7 — Engineer Wave responsibilities (NORMATIVE — Wave G binding cleanup)

The v4.0 Wave G engineer is responsible for:

1. Deleting all files / methods / symbols listed in §35.2-§35.5.
2. Removing all `#[deprecated]` attributes that tie to the deleted surface.
3. Regenerating `crates/semiflow-ffi/include/remizov.h` with v3-only surface (the bare-name `smf_*` functions remain; the `_v2` suffixed ones are gone).
4. Updating `crates/semiflow-py/src/lib.rs` to remove the `_v2` shim method declarations.
5. Updating `crates/semiflow-wasm/src/lib.rs` to remove the `*V2` shim method declarations.
6. Updating `xtask` CLI to remove the `--v2-shim` flags.
7. Updating CI to remove the `ffi-build-v2-shim`, `py-build-v2-shim`, `wasm-build-v2-shim` jobs.
8. Updating `docs/migration/v3-to-v4.md` per §"Migration window log" with the actual v4.0.0 release SHA.
9. Verifying `cargo build --no-default-features` succeeds on every workspace crate (no v2_compat feature needed).
10. Verifying G_binding_parity sub-tests 1 + 3 + 5 PASS at v3-only surface (no parallel v2 surface to cross-test against; sub-tests 2 + 4 + 6 are REMOVED from the gate).

## §36 — `LadderRung<K, F>` formal sealed typing surface (v5.0, ADR-0100, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §36.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v3.0–v4.3 ζ-ladder shipped four nested-Richardson Chernoff rungs at K=2/4/6/8 (math §27 ζ⁴ + §27.bis ζ⁶ + §27.ter ζ⁸; ADRs 0086/0088/0090). Each rung impls `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` per §26 / ADR-0073, witnessing order-K Chernoff tangency on `D(A^K)` via Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1. The structural invariant **"rung K is the canonical Richardson combination on the rung at K-2"** is currently encoded only in prose comments and per-rung constructor-parameter types; v5.0 A.6 formalises it as a sealed typing surface `LadderRung<K, F>` super-bounding `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` per ADR-0100.

### §36.2 — `LadderRung<K, F>` trait surface (NORMATIVE library)

```rust
pub trait LadderRung<const K: usize, F: SemiflowFloat = f64>:
    ApproximationSubspace<K, F> + sealed::Sealed
{
    /// Predecessor rung index, or `None` for the K=2 ladder base.
    const PREDECESSOR_K: Option<usize>;
}
```

The sealed marker (`sealed::Sealed`) restricts impls to a curated catalogue inside `semiflow-core` — see §36.4. Trait-object dispatch on `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` is preserved (no GAT, no recursive const-generic where-clauses).

### §36.3 — K → K-2 invariant (CITATION — Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1; Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 §II.4)

For each ladder rung at index $K \in \{4, 6, 8\}$, the canonical Richardson combination on the predecessor rung at index $K - 2$ cancels the leading $O(\tau^{K-1})$ symmetric global-error term, lifting Chernoff convergence order from $K - 2$ to $K$ inductively. The combination coefficient pair is $\alpha = 4^{(K/2)-1}$ and divisor $\alpha - 1$ per the standard Romberg-in-time formula:

$$
R^{K/2}(\tau) f \;=\; \frac{\alpha \cdot R^{(K-2)/2}(\tau/2)^2 \, f \;-\; R^{(K-2)/2}(\tau) \, f}{\alpha - 1}.
$$

Substituting $K = 4, 6, 8$ recovers ADR-0088 §"Algorithm" verbatim ($\alpha = 4, 16, 64$ with divisors $3, 15, 63$). The K=2 base ($R^1 \equiv \mathrm{K5}$, palindromic Strang) has no predecessor; this is the `PREDECESSOR_K = None` sentinel of §36.2. Mathematical foundation: the odd-power-only global error expansion of symmetric semigroup approximations (Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 §II.4) guarantees each Richardson level cancels exactly the leading $\tau^{K-1}$ term; Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3.1 specialised to $m = K$ certifies the corresponding Chernoff convergence rate $o(1/n^{K-1})$ on $\mathcal{D}_K = D(A^K)$.

### §36.4 — v5.0 catalogue (NORMATIVE library)

| K | Type | PREDECESSOR_K | ADR | Math §  |
|---|------|--------------|-----|---------|
| 2 | `Diffusion4thChernoff<F>`      | `None`     | 0086 | §13 (K5 palindromic Strang base) |
| 4 | `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff<F>` | `Some(2)`  | 0086 + AMENDMENT 1 | §27 (Path β) |
| 6 | `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff<F>` | `Some(4)`  | 0088 + AMENDMENT 1 | §27.bis      |
| 8 | `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff<F>` | `Some(6)`  | 0088 + AMENDMENT 2 + 0090 | §27.ter |

The catalogue is closed at v5.0; future rungs (e.g., K=10 ζ¹⁰ at v5.x conditional on $D(A^{10})$ smoothness budget feasibility) require ADR + sealed impl block inside `semiflow-core` per ADR-0100 §"Decision".

### §36.5 — T_LADDER_RUNG sympy oracle (NORMATIVE library)

Build-time sympy verification at `scripts/verify_ladder_rung.py` (4 sub-checks; mirrors T23N_zeta6/T23N_zeta8 sibling pattern per ADR-0088):

- **(a)** **Catalogue completeness**: exactly 4 sealed impls in the catalogue, indexed at K ∈ {2, 4, 6, 8}.
- **(b)** **Unique base**: exactly one rung has `PREDECESSOR_K == None`; that rung is K=2.
- **(c)** **K → K-2 invariant**: for each K ∈ {4, 6, 8}, `PREDECESSOR_K == Some(K - 2)` and the predecessor at K-2 is itself in the catalogue.
- **(d)** **Richardson coefficient identity**: for each K ∈ {4, 6, 8}, the predecessor's `apply_into` combined under the standard Romberg coefficient pair $(\alpha, \alpha - 1)$ with $\alpha = 4^{(K/2)-1}$ produces the canonical order-K Richardson combination per §36.3.

Sub-checks (a)-(c) are static (catalogue introspection via build-time `cargo expand` or per-rung Rust source-text scan); sub-check (d) is symbolic Taylor-expansion verification using `sympy.Symbol("tau")` per the T23N pattern. Gate severity: **RELEASE_BLOCKING** per ADR-0100 §"Acceptance gates added".

### §36.6 — Relationship to ADR-0073 `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` (NORMATIVE library)

`LadderRung<K, F>` super-bounds `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` — every ladder rung is automatically a K-jet witness per §26, but NOT every `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` impl is a ladder rung. Non-rung impls preserved from v3.0:

- `DiffusionChernoff<F>` impls `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` (v0.3.0 ζ-A τ²-correction; semantically orthogonal to the Richardson ladder per ADR-0088 cross-reference list — NOT a `LadderRung<2, F>`).
- `TruncatedExp4thDiffusionChernoff<F>` impls `ApproximationSubspace<6, F>` (v0.6.0 ζ⁴ witness consumer; consumed by `Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff::new` per ADR-0075/0086 — NOT a `LadderRung<6, F>`).
- `KolmogorovHypoelliptic<F>` impls `ApproximationSubspace<2, F>` (v3.1 Hörmander-track; semantically orthogonal — NOT a `LadderRung<2, F>`).

The sealed marker `sealed::Sealed` enforces the catalogue closure: non-rung impls of `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` are not affected by ADR-0100 and continue to compile UNCHANGED.

### §36.7 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **K=10 / K=12 rungs** — conditional on D(A^{10}) / D(A^{12}) smoothness budget feasibility (per ADR-0088 AMENDMENT 2 floor-cascade diagnosis); requires architect ADR + sealed impl block + T_LADDER_RUNG catalogue update + corresponding §27.quater / §27.quinquies math section. Out-of-scope for v5.0.
- **Padé rungs (B.1 ADR-0101)** — Padé operates by scaling-and-squaring on the matrix exponential, NOT by Richardson on a symmetric base; the K → K-2 invariant does not apply. Padé is a separate approximation family and does NOT impl `LadderRung<K, F>` even if it ships at v5.0 Path α/β/γ per ADR-0101.
- **Cross-domain ladders** (2D / 3D / manifold rungs) — out-of-scope per ADR-0088 §"Out of scope"; the v5.0 catalogue is 1D-divergence-form only.

### §36.8 — References

- ADR-0073 — `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` super-bounded by this section.
- ADR-0086 + AMENDMENT 1 — Path β Richardson on K5 (K=2 base).
- ADR-0088 + AMENDMENT 1/2 — ζ⁶ + ζ⁸ rungs (K=6, K=8 populating ADRs).
- ADR-0090 — v4.3 ζ⁸ Chebyshev-base K=8 rung shipping.
- ADR-0100 (this section's contract authority).
- math.md §26 — `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` semantics (reused verbatim).
- math.md §27 / §27.bis / §27.ter — per-rung algorithm specs (referenced by the catalogue table §36.4).
- Galkin-Remizov 2025 *Israel J. Math.* — *Tangency of Chernoff approximations to operator semigroups on Banach spaces*, Theorem 3.1.
- Richardson 1911 — *The approximate arithmetical solution by finite differences of physical problems*, **Phil. Trans. R. Soc. A** 210, pp. 307–357.
- Romberg 1955 — *Vereinfachte numerische Integration*, **Det Kongelige Norske Videnskabers Selskab Forhandlinger** 28, pp. 30–36.
- Hairer-Lubich-Wanner 2006 — *Geometric Numerical Integration*, **Springer Series in Computational Mathematics** 31, §II.4.

## §37 (corrected v6.2.4) — Subordinated Chernoff: Bochner-Phillips density quadrature

A Bernstein/Laplace exponent φ(λ)=bλ+∫₀^∞(1−e^{−sλ})ν(ds) defines the subordinated semigroup exp(−τφ(A)) with generator −φ(A) = −bA − ∫₀^∞(I−e^{−sA})ν(ds). The order-1 Chernoff tangent MUST satisfy F^φ(τ) = I − τφ(A) + o(τ), which is NONLINEAR in A and CANNOT be produced by any single generator-scaling c·τ·A (the v4.8 error; see ADR-0103 Amendment 1). Correct construction (Bochner-Phillips, exact in s where a density exists): for a subordinator S_τ with density f_τ(s) satisfying E[e^{−λ S_τ}]=e^{−τφ(λ)}, exp(−τφ(A)) = ∫₀^∞ e^{−sA} f_τ(s) ds, so F^φ(τ):=Σ_k w_k e^{−s_k A} with (s_k,w_k) a quadrature of f_τ (w_k≥0, Σw_k=1) satisfies Σ_k w_k e^{−λ s_k} ≈ e^{−τφ(λ)} for ALL eigenvalues λ. Per backend: Gamma φ_c(λ)=log(1+λ/c): S_τ~Γ(shape=τ,rate=c), generalized Gauss-Laguerre(param=τ−1), exact in s. InverseGaussian φ_c(λ)=√(c²+2λ)−c: S_τ~IG(τ/c,τ²), truncated standardized-IG Gauss rule (KNOWN LIMITATION v6.2.4: over-decays for small τ due to the Pinsky 1986 s^{−3/2} head — deferred, not yet correct). Stable φ_α(λ)=λ^α (no elementary density): regularized Lévy integrand (1−e^{−sλ})/s via generalized Gauss-Laguerre(−α), order-1 to the correct exp(−τλ^α) for all λ. Gate G_SUBORD_ORDER1 (RELEASE_BLOCKING): 5-eigenvalue sweep λ∈{4,8,16,32,48}, oracle exact=exp(−φ(λ_i)) vs wrong=exp(−φ(1)·λ_i) per mode, single n=128 point (NO n-sweep — quadrature is exact-in-s for Gamma/IG so no τ-convergence rate exists); assert (A) |f_128−exact|≤5e-3·max(1,φ(λ)) AND (B) |f_128−exact|<0.2·|f_128−wrong| for ALL 5 λ; ≥2-of-3 backends (Stable+Gamma pass; IG deferred). The old single-μ=1 gate is RETIRED.

### §37.1 — Lévy subordinators and CBF admissibility (NORMATIVE library scope)

A **one-dimensional Lévy subordinator** is a càdlàg stochastic process $(S_t)_{t \geq 0}$ with values in $[0, \infty)$, $S_0 = 0$, independent and non-negative stationary increments. Its law is characterised by the **Laplace exponent** $\varphi : (0, \infty) \to (0, \infty)$ via

$$
\mathbb{E}\bigl[\exp(-\lambda S_t)\bigr] \;=\; \exp\bigl(-t\, \varphi(\lambda)\bigr), \qquad \lambda > 0, \; t \geq 0. \tag{37.1}
$$

The set of admissible $\varphi$ is exactly the **Complete Bernstein Functions** (CBF; Schilling-Song-Vondraček 2012 §13), characterised by

- (CBF1) $\varphi(0) = 0$ (no killing at $t = 0$),
- (CBF2) $\varphi$ is concave-increasing on $(0, \infty)$,
- (CBF3) $(-1)^{k+1} \varphi^{(k)}(\lambda) \geq 0$ for all $\lambda > 0$ and all $k \in \mathbb{N}_{\geq 1}$.

The three concrete backends (`StableSubordinator`, `GammaSubordinator`, `InverseGaussianSubordinator`) are all CBF — see §37.5.

### §37.2 — Bochner-Phillips functional calculus (CITATION — Bochner 1949, Phillips 1952)

Given a strongly-continuous semigroup $(T_t)_{t \geq 0}$ on a Banach space $X$ with generator $A$, and a Lévy subordinator $(S_t)$ with Laplace exponent $\varphi$, the **subordinate semigroup** is

$$
T^\varphi_t f \;:=\; \mathbb{E}[T_{S_t} f] \;=\; \int_0^\infty T_s f \; \mu^\varphi_t(\mathrm{d}s), \tag{37.2}
$$

where $\mu^\varphi_t$ is the law of $S_t$ (a probability measure on $[0, \infty)$ with Laplace transform $\exp(-t \varphi(\cdot))$). The Phillips functional calculus (Phillips 1952 Theorem 1.1) yields that $T^\varphi$ is itself a strongly continuous semigroup with generator $-\varphi(-A)$ (defined via the CBF Bochner integral over the resolvent — see Schilling-Song-Vondraček 2012 §13.3 for the operator-domain construction).

**Key example** (α-stable, $A = \Delta$, $\varphi(\lambda) = \lambda^\alpha$): $T^\varphi_t = \exp\bigl(-t \,(-\Delta)^\alpha\bigr)$, the **Riesz fractional heat semigroup** for $\alpha \in (0, 1)$.

### §37.3 — Butko 2018 Theorem 2.1 — order-1 Chernoff tangency (CITATION — Butko 2018 §4)

Let $F : [0, \infty) \to \mathcal{B}(X)$ be a Chernoff approximation of $T_t$ (i.e., $F(0) = I$, $F'(0)|_{\text{strong}} = A$, and $\|F(s)\| \leq \exp(s \omega)$ for some $\omega \in \mathbb{R}$). Define the **subordinated Chernoff family**

$$
F^\varphi(\tau) f \;:=\; \int_0^\infty F(s) f \; \mu^\varphi_\tau(\mathrm{d}s). \tag{37.3}
$$

**Theorem (Butko 2018 §4 Theorem 2.1)**: $F^\varphi$ is a Chernoff approximation of the subordinate semigroup $T^\varphi$:

- $F^\varphi(0) = I$ trivially;
- $(F^\varphi)'(0)|_{\text{strong}} = -\varphi(-A)$;
- $\bigl\| F^\varphi(\tau/n) \bigr\|^n \to T^\varphi_\tau$ strongly as $n \to \infty$ (Chernoff product formula).

The order of $F^\varphi$ as a Chernoff approximation is **exactly 1** (Butko 2018 §4 Remark following Thm 2.1) — higher-order subordinated Chernoff is research-open. The module ships order-1 only; higher-order extensions are out-of-scope per ADR-0103 §"Out of scope".

**v6.2.4 correctness note**: The original v4.8 implementation used generator-scaled GL32 nodes (`s_k = GL32_NODES[k]·φ(1)·τ`) which linearize φ to a constant slope, producing exp(−Tφ(1)A) rather than exp(−Tφ(A)). This was correct only at λ=1. Fixed in v6.2.4 via Bochner-Phillips density quadrature (ADR-0103 Amendment 1). The eigensolver infrastructure is now in `gen_quadrature.rs`.

### §37.4 — Growth bound (NORMATIVE library)

If the base Chernoff $F$ satisfies $\|F(s)\| \leq \exp(s \omega)$ for $s \geq 0$ and some $\omega \in \mathbb{R}$, then the subordinated Chernoff $F^\varphi$ satisfies

$$
\bigl\|F^\varphi(\tau)\bigr\| \;\leq\; \int_0^\infty \exp(s \omega) \, \mu^\varphi_\tau(\mathrm{d}s) \;=\; \exp\bigl(\tau \, \varphi(\omega)\bigr) \qquad (\omega < 0). \tag{37.4}
$$

For $\omega \geq 0$ the integral in (37.4) may diverge; in that case the growth bound is $\exp(\tau \, \varphi^*(\omega))$ where $\varphi^*$ is the analytic continuation of $\varphi$ to the right half-plane (CBF: $\varphi$ extends analytically to $\{\text{Re}(\lambda) > 0\}$ — Schilling-Song-Vondraček 2012 Proposition 3.6). The library's `growth()` implementation passes through the base growth as a conservative placeholder; tight subordinator-aware growth bounds are RESEARCH-OPEN per the same Butko 2018 §5 future work.

### §37.5 — Three concrete CBF backends (NORMATIVE library)

| Backend | Laplace exponent $\varphi(\lambda)$ | Density $p_\tau(s)$, $s > 0$ | CBF citation | v6.2.4 status |
|---------|-------------------------------------|-------------------------------|--------------|----------------|
| `StableSubordinator { alpha }` | $\lambda^\alpha$, $\alpha \in (0, 1)$ | no elementary form; regularized Lévy integrand $(1-e^{-s\lambda})/s$ via gen-GL(−α) | SSV 2012 Example 14.3 | CORRECT |
| `GammaSubordinator { c }` | $\log(1 + \lambda / c)$, $c > 0$ | $\tfrac{c^\tau s^{\tau-1} e^{-c s}}{\Gamma(\tau)}$; gen-GL(τ−1) exact | SSV 2012 Example 14.4 | CORRECT |
| `InverseGaussianSubordinator { c }` | $\sqrt{c^2 + 2\lambda} - c$, $c > 0$ | $\tfrac{\tau}{\sqrt{2\pi s^3}} e^{- (\tau - c s)^2 / (2 s)}$; truncated IG Gauss rule | SSV 2012 Example 14.5 | KNOWN-FAILING (deferred; Pinsky 1986 s^{−3/2} head over-decays for small τ) |

The CBF admissibility for each backend is verified symbolically in `T_SUBORD` sub-check (1) by checking $\varphi(0) = 0$ and $(-1)^{k+1} \varphi^{(k)}(\lambda) \geq 0$ for $k = 1, \ldots, 4$ at a representative $\lambda > 0$.

### §37.6 — Quadrature: generalized Gauss-Laguerre via Golub-Welsch (NORMATIVE library — corrected v6.2.4)

The subordinated integral (37.3) is evaluated by quadrature of the subordinator density $f_\tau(s)$ directly (Bochner-Phillips exact identity). The Golub-Welsch symmetric-tridiagonal eigensolver and generalized Gauss-Laguerre construction are in `gen_quadrature.rs`. Per-backend rule:

- **`StableSubordinator { alpha }`** — no closed-form density; uses generalized Gauss-Laguerre(−α) on the regularized Lévy integrand $(1 - e^{-s\lambda})/s$, achieving order-1 tangency to $e^{-\tau\lambda^\alpha}$ for ALL $\lambda$.
- **`GammaSubordinator { c }`** — $S_\tau \sim \Gamma(\text{shape}=\tau, \text{rate}=c)$; generalized Gauss-Laguerre(param=τ−1), exact in $s$.
- **`InverseGaussianSubordinator { c }`** — $S_\tau \sim \text{IG}(\tau/c, \tau^2)$; truncated standardized-IG Gauss rule. **KNOWN LIMITATION (v6.2.4, deferred)**: over-decays for small per-step $\tau$ due to the Pinsky 1986 $s^{-3/2}$ singularity at the head of the IG density; the IG backend converges to the wrong limit and is explicitly flagged KNOWN-FAILING pending a future fix.

The old v4.8 GL32 `resolvent_quad.rs` table is no longer used for the density quadrature nodes (the Golub-Welsch construction generates $\tau$-dependent nodes). The `GL32_NODES` / `GL32_WEIGHTS` constants remain in `resolvent_quad.rs` for the Laplace-Chernoff Resolvent (ADR-0069).

### §37.7 — Implementation map (NORMATIVE library)

- **File**: `crates/semiflow-core/src/subordinated.rs`.
- **Quadrature infrastructure**: `crates/semiflow-core/src/gen_quadrature.rs` (Golub-Welsch + generalized Gauss-Laguerre; extracted at v6.2.4).
- **Trait**: `LevySubordinator<F>` (sibling-to-`BoundedGeometryManifold<F>` pattern from ADR-0071).
- **Concrete impls**: `StableSubordinator<F>` (CORRECT), `GammaSubordinator<F>` (CORRECT), `InverseGaussianSubordinator<F>` (KNOWN-FAILING — IG deferred).
- **Generic wrapper**: `SubordinatedChernoff<C, S, F>` where `C: ChernoffFunction<F>, S: LevySubordinator<F>` — itself impl `ChernoffFunction<F>` with `order() = 1`.
- **Test gates**: `T_SUBORD` (NORMATIVE sympy oracle, 5 sub-checks — `scripts/verify_subordinated_chernoff.py`); `G_SUBORD_ORDER1` (RELEASE_BLOCKING; 5-eigenvalue sweep λ∈{4,8,16,32,48}, correct-limit assert, ≥2/3 backends — `tests/subordinated_order1_slope.rs`); `subordinated_does_not_linearize_phi` (always-on anti-regression — `tests/subordinated_order1_slope.rs`).

### §37.8 — Relationship to v3.0 `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` and v5.0 `LadderRung<K, F>` (NORMATIVE library)

- **Not a `LadderRung<K, F>`** (ADR-0100): the sealed v5.0 ladder catalogue contains only diagonal Richardson rungs at K ∈ {2, 4, 6, 8}; `SubordinatedChernoff` is order-1 and lives outside the Richardson family.
- **Not a `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` impl** (ADR-0073): the subordinated approximation is order-1 and would impl `ApproximationSubspace<1, F>` — but the K = 1 marker is not part of the v3.0+ catalogue (which starts at K = 2). A future minor MAY add a `ApproximationSubspace<1, F>` marker if order-1 witnesses become an explicit Galkin-Remizov 2025 §3.1 use case; that decision is deferred.

### §37.9 — References

- Butko 2018 — *Chernoff Approximation of Subordinate Semigroups*, **Stochastics and Dynamics** 18 (3), §4 Theorem 2.1 (the primary citation; defines the order-1 Chernoff tangency).
- Bochner 1949 — *Diffusion equation and stochastic processes*, **PNAS** 35 (5), pp. 368–370 (subordination via Lévy measures).
- Phillips 1952 — *On the generation of semigroups of linear operators*, **Pacific J. Math.** 2, pp. 343–369 (functional calculus for CBF of generators).
- Sato 1999 — *Lévy Processes and Infinitely Divisible Distributions*, **Cambridge Studies in Advanced Math.** 68, §30 (full Lévy-process foundation).
- Schilling-Song-Vondraček 2012 — *Bernstein Functions: Theory and Applications*, **de Gruyter Studies in Math.** 37, §13 (CBF criterion + examples used in §37.5).
- Pinsky 1986 — *Lectures on Random Evolution*, **World Scientific** §V.3 (IG density s^{−3/2} singularity; motivation for KNOWN LIMITATION deferral).
- Abramowitz-Stegun 1964 — *Handbook of Mathematical Functions*, **National Bureau of Standards** 55, Table 25.9 (Gauss-Laguerre 32-pt nodes/weights; retained in `resolvent_quad.rs` for ADR-0069 Resolvent).
- Madan-Carr-Chang 1998 — *The variance gamma process and option pricing*, **Eur. Finance Review** 2 (motivating example for `GammaSubordinator`).
- Barndorff-Nielsen 1997 — *Normal inverse Gaussian distributions and stochastic volatility modelling*, **Scand. J. Statist.** 24 (motivating example for `InverseGaussianSubordinator`).
- ADR-0069 — v2.7 Laplace-Chernoff Resolvent (GL32 quadrature retained in `resolvent_quad.rs`).
- ADR-0071 — v2.8 Manifold sibling pattern (trait + concretes + wrapper REUSED).
- ADR-0073 — v3.0 `ApproximationSubspace<K, F>` (relationship in §37.8).
- ADR-0078 — v3.1 quantum-graph standalone kernel (separate-module pattern REUSED).
- ADR-0098 — v4.6 Robin BC partial-additive port (PRE-FLIGHT + standalone-kernel pattern REUSED).

- ADR-0103 Amendment 1 (correctness fix authority for this section).

## §38 — Adjoint Fokker-Planck Chernoff on weak-* topology of M(ℝ^d) (post-v5.0, ADR-0107, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics — MATH CREATION)

### §38.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The library's catalogue through v5.0 contains **primal** Chernoff functions only: approximation of the Banach-space semigroup `e^{tL}` on `C_b(ℝ^d)` or `L^2(ℝ^d)` in operator-norm convergence (per Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 explicit-constants formulation, ADR-0106). The DUAL semigroup `e^{tL*}` acts on the signed-measure space `M(ℝ^d)` (forward Fokker-Planck / Kolmogorov forward equation, NOT to be confused with backward Kolmogorov which is the primal `e^{tL}` evolving expected values of test functions). The dual evolution is the natural setting for probability-density-evolution applications: diffusion of a probability mass, transport of a signed charge density, dual variational problems in optimal transport.

The question A.1 from the v2.6 → v4.0 academic-priority roadmap (`~/.claude/plans/roadmap-reflective-biscuit.md`) asked: **does Chernoff approximation extend to the dual semigroup e^{tL*} on M(ℝ^d) under the vague (weak-*) topology σ(M, C_b)?** Per Phase A literature scan (ADR-0107), no paper in the project's `.dev-docs/papers/` collection addresses this question; the Chernoff approximation literature (Chernoff 1968, Galkin-Remizov 2025, Butko 2018, MMRS 2023, BLU 2007, Vedenin 2020) addresses primal Banach-space convergence only. ADR-0107 supplies the math via a dual-pairing construction.

### §38.2 — Dual-pairing construction (CITATION — Pazy 1983 §1.4 + Bogachev 2007 §4)

Let `(C_b(ℝ^d), ‖·‖_∞)` denote the Banach space of bounded continuous functions, and `(M(ℝ^d), ‖·‖_TV)` the dual space of signed Borel measures of bounded variation. The dual pairing is

$$\langle f, \rho \rangle := \int_{\mathbb{R}^d} f \, d\rho, \quad f \in C_b(\mathbb{R}^d), \; \rho \in M(\mathbb{R}^d).$$

For any bounded linear `S : C_b(ℝ^d) → C_b(ℝ^d)` (forward Chernoff function at fixed time `t`), the formal adjoint `S* : M(ℝ^d) → M(ℝ^d)` is defined by

$$\langle f, S^* \rho \rangle := \langle S f, \rho \rangle \quad \forall f \in C_b(\mathbb{R}^d), \; \rho \in M(\mathbb{R}^d).$$

By the Hahn-Banach theorem applied to `(C_b, M)` duality (Bogachev 2007 §4 Theorem 4.1.5), `S*` exists and is unique with operator norm `‖S*‖_{M→M} = ‖S‖_{C_b→C_b}`. The **vague topology** on `M(ℝ^d)` is the weakest topology making each pairing `ρ ↦ ⟨f, ρ⟩` continuous for `f ∈ C_b(ℝ^d)`; it is the canonical setting for convergence of measures arising from the dual of `C_b`.

### §38.3 — Lemma A.1 (Theorem 4 adjoint kernel; NORMATIVE library)

Let `S(t)f(x) = (1/4)f(x+h) + (1/4)f(x-h) + (1/2)f(x+k) + tc·f(x)` with `h = 2√(at)`, `k = 2bt`, and `a, b, c` constants (the Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 4 Chernoff function, eq. 11, with multiplicative-form generator `A·φ = a·φ'' + b·φ' + c·φ`). Then for all `ρ ∈ M(ℝ)`,

$$S^*(t) \rho = \tfrac{1}{4}\tau_{+h}\rho + \tfrac{1}{4}\tau_{-h}\rho + \tfrac{1}{2}\tau_{+k}\rho + tc \cdot \rho$$

where `(τ_a ρ)(B) := ρ(B - a)` is the push-forward of `ρ` by shift `+a`.

**Proof** (sympy-verified at `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS.theorem4_chernoff_adjoint`, sub-check (b)):

By dual-pairing definition and Fubini:

$$\langle f, S^*(t)\rho \rangle = \langle S(t)f, \rho \rangle = \int \left[ \tfrac{1}{4}f(x+h) + \tfrac{1}{4}f(x-h) + \tfrac{1}{2}f(x+k) + tc \cdot f(x) \right] d\rho(x).$$

Substituting `y = x + h` in the first integral (the measure `ρ` transforms via push-forward `(τ_{+h}ρ)(B) = ρ(B - h)`):

$$\int f(x+h) \, d\rho(x) = \int f(y) \, d(\tau_{+h}\rho)(y).$$

Identical substitution for `y = x - h`, `y = x + k`, with the constant-term `tc·f(x)` unchanged. Identifying coefficients with the dual-pairing template `⟨f, S^*(t)\rho⟩ = ⟨f, (1/4)τ_{+h}\rho + (1/4)τ_{-h}\rho + (1/2)τ_{+k}\rho + tc·\rho⟩` gives the claim. ∎

**Variable-coefficient case**: For `a(x), b(x), c(x)` smooth, the structure is identical with x-dependent push-forward distances at each mass point: the Dirac at `x` is push-forwarded to `x ± 2√(a(x)·t)`, `x + 2b(x)·t`, with weight (1/4, 1/4, 1/2) and a reweighted-by-`(1 + t·c(x))` Dirac at `x` itself.

### §38.4 — Theorem A.2 (Vague-topology rate transfer; NORMATIVE library)

Suppose `S(t)` is a Chernoff function satisfying Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 with `m`-tangency hypothesis (eq. 7) and conclusion (eq. 8):

$$\|S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f\|_{C_b} \le \frac{M_1 M_2 t^{m+1} e^{wt}}{n^m} \sum_{j=0}^{m+p} e^{-wt/n} C_j(t/n) \|L^j f\|.$$

Then for all `ρ ∈ M(ℝ^d)` with `‖ρ‖_TV < ∞`, the adjoint `S*(t)` satisfies the IDENTICAL rate on the vague topology, modulated by `‖ρ‖_TV`:

$$\left| \langle f, S^*(t/n)^n \rho - e^{tL^*} \rho \rangle \right| \le \frac{M_1 M_2 t^{m+1} e^{wt}}{n^m} \left( \sum_{j=0}^{m+p} e^{-wt/n} C_j(t/n) \|L^j f\| \right) \cdot \|\rho\|_{TV}$$

for all `f ∈ C_b^{m+p}(ℝ^d)` with bounded `L^j f`.

**Proof** (sympy-verified at `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS.theorem3_dual_rate`, sub-check (f)):

By the dual-pairing identity (§38.2):

$$\left| \langle f, S^*(t/n)^n \rho - e^{tL^*} \rho \rangle \right| = \left| \langle S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f, \rho \rangle \right|.$$

By Hölder duality on `(C_b, M)` (Bogachev 2007 §4 eq. 4.1.5):

$$\left| \langle g, \rho \rangle \right| \le \|g\|_{C_b} \cdot \|\rho\|_{TV} \quad \forall g \in C_b(\mathbb{R}^d), \rho \in M(\mathbb{R}^d).$$

Applying this to `g = S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f` and substituting the Galkin-Remizov 2025 Theorem 3 bound:

$$\left| \langle f, S^*(t/n)^n \rho - e^{tL^*} \rho \rangle \right| \le \|S(t/n)^n f - e^{tL} f\|_{C_b} \cdot \|\rho\|_{TV} \le \frac{M_1 M_2 t^{m+1} e^{wt}}{n^m} \left( \cdots \right) \|\rho\|_{TV}. \quad \blacksquare$$

Theorem A.2 is COMPOSITIONAL: EVERY primal Chernoff function in the v2.6 → v5.x catalogue (DiffusionChernoff with `m=1`, Diffusion4thChernoff with `m=2`, Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff Path β with `m=3`, manifold backends, Hörmander backends, quantum-graph kernels) AUTOMATICALLY induces a corresponding adjoint Chernoff function with IDENTICAL rate. This is high architectural leverage from the dual-pairing argument; the engineer wave can implement a SINGLE GENERIC WRAPPER `AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff<C, F, D>` that lifts any forward `ChernoffFunction<F>` to its dual.

### §38.5 — Lemma A.3 (Uniform tightness of iterated S*; NORMATIVE library)

For `ρ_0 ∈ M(ℝ)` with finite second moment `M_2(ρ_0) := ∫ x² dρ_0 < ∞`, the iterated adjoint `S*(t/n)^n ρ_0` satisfies

$$\int x^2 \, d(S^*(t/n)^n \rho_0) \le \int x^2 \, d\rho_0 + (4 a t + 4 b^2 t^2) \cdot \|\rho_0\|_{TV}$$

UNIFORMLY in `n`.

**Proof** (sympy-verified at `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS.tightness_propagation`, sub-check (d)):

Compute `S(t)(x²)(x)` directly:

$$S(t)(x^2)(x) = \tfrac{1}{4}(x+h)^2 + \tfrac{1}{4}(x-h)^2 + \tfrac{1}{2}(x+k)^2 + tc \cdot x^2 = (1 + tc) x^2 + 2 b t \cdot x + 2 a t + 2 b^2 t^2.$$

The variance accumulation per step (at `c = 0`, mass-conservative case) is `Δσ² = 2a·τ`. After `n` steps with `τ = t/n`, the total variance accumulation is `n · 2a · (t/n) = 2at`, INDEPENDENT of `n`. Combined with the drift contribution `2b²t²` from the `k = 2bt` Dirac, the total second-moment increment per iteration of `S*(t/n)^n` is bounded by `(4at + 4b²t²) · ‖ρ_0‖_{TV}`. ∎

By Prokhorov's theorem (Bogachev 2007 §8 Theorem 8.6.2), Lemma A.3 implies the family `{S*(t/n)^n ρ_0}_{n ≥ 1}` is UNIFORMLY TIGHT; combined with the rate of Theorem A.2 (which provides Cauchy-style convergence), this gives existence of a unique vague-topology limit equal to `e^{tL*}ρ_0` (the forward Fokker-Planck semigroup, well-defined by Pazy 1983 §1.4).

### §38.6 — Total mass conservation (NORMATIVE library)

The adjoint Chernoff function `S*(t)` preserves total mass up to the multiplicative reweighting:

$$\int_{\mathbb{R}^d} d(S^*(t)\rho) = (1 + tc) \int_{\mathbb{R}^d} d\rho.$$

**Proof** (sympy-verified at `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS.total_mass_conservation`, sub-check (c)):

Sum the four Dirac-pushforward coefficients: `(1/4) + (1/4) + (1/2) + tc = 1 + tc`. When `c = 0`, total mass is EXACTLY conserved (Markov semigroup). When `c ≤ 0`, the semigroup is sub-stochastic (mass-leaking; corresponds to killing-rate `|c|` in the Fokker-Planck equation). ∎

### §38.7 — Canonical example: 1D Brownian motion (CITATION — Itô calculus + classical heat equation)

For 1D Brownian motion (the canonical Fokker-Planck instance), `a = 1/2`, `b = 0`, `c = 0`, so `L = (1/2)∂²_x` is the standard Wiener-process generator. The forward Fokker-Planck adjoint semigroup applied to `ρ_0 = δ_0` (point mass at origin) is the centred Gaussian `e^{tL*}δ_0 = N(0, t)`.

The adjoint Chernoff function from Lemma A.1 (with `h = √(2t)`, `k = 0`, `c = 0`) is the symmetric 3-point Bernoulli measure:

$$S^*(t)\delta_0 = \tfrac{1}{4}\delta_{+\sqrt{2t}} + \tfrac{1}{4}\delta_{-\sqrt{2t}} + \tfrac{1}{2}\delta_0.$$

This has first moment `0` and variance `(1/4)·2t + (1/4)·2t + (1/2)·0 = t`. By CLT-style argument (sympy-verified at `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS.vague_convergence_brownian`, sub-check (e)), the `n`-step iterate's characteristic function converges to the Gaussian characteristic function:

$$\widehat{S^*(t/n)^n \delta_0}(\xi) = \left[ \tfrac{1}{2} \cos(\xi \sqrt{2t/n}) + \tfrac{1}{2} \right]^n = \left[ 1 - \tfrac{\xi^2 t}{2 n} + O(n^{-2}) \right]^n \xrightarrow{n \to \infty} e^{-\xi^2 t / 2} = \widehat{N(0, t)}(\xi).$$

By Lévy's continuity theorem (Bogachev 2007 §5 Theorem 5.5.1), the iterated adjoint converges to the Gaussian `N(0, t)` in distribution = in vague topology. This concrete instance reproduces the classical heat-kernel limit and grounds the engineer-wave numerical implementation.

### §38.8 — T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS sympy oracle (NORMATIVE library)

The 6 sub-checks of `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS` formally verify the constructions of §38.3 – §38.7. See `scripts/verify_adjoint_fp_tightness.py` and `contracts/semiflow-core.properties.yaml` entry `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS`. PRE-FLIGHT 6/6 PASS verified 2026-05-30; integrated into `cargo run -p xtask -- test-fast` sympy sweep; failure BLOCKS v5.1+ release.

### §38.9 — Engineer-wave AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff (NORMATIVE library — IMPLEMENTING in v8.0.0)

The engineer wave at `.dev-docs/specs/adjoint-fp-wave.md` documents the `AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff<C, F, const D: usize>` Rust implementation:
- **State type**: NEW `MeasureState<F, D>` — sparse 4-Dirac-pushforward + Gaussian-smoothed-background representation.
- **Wrapper**: `AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff<C, F, D>` is generic over forward `C : Adjointable<F, D>` (compositional per Theorem A.2).
- **Super-trait**: `Adjointable<F, D>` with blanket impl for every forward `ChernoffFunction<F>` via the Theorem 4 dual-pairing form.
- **Engineer-wave gate**: `G_ADJOINT_FP_ORDER` (RELEASE_BLOCKING; vague-convergence slope ≤ −0.95 on iterated Brownian-motion characteristic-function self-convergence at `n ∈ {16, 32, 64, 128, 256}` PLUS a discrete-adjoint-identity smoke ⟨L*u,v⟩=⟨u,Lv⟩ < 1e-12). Materialises the v6.0.0 RESERVED `G_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS_VAGUE` stub.
- **Module**: `crates/semiflow-core/src/adjoint_fp.rs` (Cohort 13 pre-allocated this name).
- **v8.0.0 status (Phase-4 item C2, IMPLEMENTING — ADR-0107 AMENDMENT 1):** the user opted the engineer wave into v8.0.0 (synergy with F1 differentiable Chernoff — a measure-side adjoint complements the `Dual<F>` function-side forward-mode AD for sensitivity workflows). The §38 math (Lemmas A.1, A.3; Theorem A.2; mass conservation; Brownian example) and the `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS` sympy oracle (6/6 PASS, re-confirmed 2026-06-07) are UNCHANGED — no new math or oracle is authored at v8.0.0; the wave materialises the existing blueprint as Rust + the `G_ADJOINT_FP_ORDER` numerical gate. The Dirac-count $4^{n}$ blow-up (spec §"Per-step cost") is sidestepped at the gate by the characteristic-function analytical Dirac-fold (⟨cos(ξx), Σwᵢδ_{xᵢ}⟩ = Σwᵢcos(ξxᵢ), O(n_diracs) cost); long-time applications use the Gaussian-smoothed background + weighted-Voronoi reduction. NOT confused with the shipped `AdjointChernoff` (§15, ADR-0114): that is the dual semigroup $S^*(\tau)=\exp(\tau A^T)$ on the SAME $L^2$/$C_b$ function space (backward Cauchy problem); §38 is the dual on the MEASURE space $M(\mathbb{R}^d)$ with a `MeasureState` — a different object.

### §38.10 — Future extensions (NORMATIVE library — out-of-scope notes)

- **Wasserstein-topology sibling**: ADR-0108 candidate (research-track only). Builds on the dual-pairing framework with `Lip₁` test functions and Kantorovich-Rubinstein duality (Bogachev 2007 §10). Different topology (strictly stronger than vague); different rate constant `‖ρ‖_{W_1}` instead of `‖ρ‖_{TV}`.
- **JKO variational scheme**: research-track only. Discretises Fokker-Planck via Wasserstein-gradient-flow steps (Jordan-Kinderlehrer-Otto 1998 *SIAM J. Math. Anal.* 29). Complementary to Chernoff approximation; out-of-scope sibling.
- **Stochastic-particle methods**: research-track only. Random-particle approximation per Bossy 2005 / Jourdain-Méléard-Woyczynski 2008. Different convergence class (stochastic distributional convergence); the deterministic Dirac-pushforward of Lemma A.1 is a noise-removed algebraic baseline.
- **Higher-order adjoint rate via Path β + Richardson dual-pairing**: structurally identical to the primal Path β construction (ADR-0086) at the dual level. Engineer-wave optional refinement; not needed for v5.1 first ship.

- Bogachev 2007 — *Measure Theory* (Volume I), **Springer**, §4 (total-variation norm, Hölder duality eq. 4.1.5), §5 (Lévy's continuity theorem), §8 (Prokhorov's theorem).

- Jordan-Kinderlehrer-Otto 1998 — *The variational formulation of the Fokker-Planck equation*, **SIAM J. Math. Anal.** 29, 1–17 (JKO scheme, out-of-scope sibling).

### §38.12 — Variance diagnostic on MeasureState (NORMATIVE library; issue #3)

Three public diagnostic methods on `MeasureState<F, D>` (all in `adjoint_fp.rs`):

**first_moment** — mass-weighted centre of mass, per axis (D-vector):
`E[x_d] = (Σ_diracs w·pos[d] + Σ_gauss w·mean[d]) / mass`, where `mass = total_variation()`.
Returns `[0; D]` when `mass = 0` (zero measure has undefined mean; zero is the safe default).

**variance** — total scalar variance (E[|x|²]−|E[x]|²):
`Var = second_moment() / mass − Σ_d (first_moment[d])²`.
Uses the mass-normalised second moment (§38.5 Lemma A.3 defines the unnormalised `⟨|x|²,ρ⟩`; division by `mass` gives E[|x|²]).
Returns `0` when `mass = 0`.

**variance_per_axis** — per-axis variance (D-vector):
`Var_d = (Σ_diracs w·pos[d]² + Σ_gauss w·(mean[d]²+var)) / mass − (E[x_d])²`.
For isotropic Gaussian covariance `σ²·I`, `Σ_d Var_d = Var` exactly (no cross-terms).
Returns `[0; D]` when `mass = 0`.

**Oracle**: `scripts/verify_measure_state_variance.py` — `T_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE` sympy gate (4/4 sub-checks: `closed_form_var`, `per_axis_var`, `var_equals_sum_per_axis`, `zero_mass_guard`). PASS verified 2026-06-23; integrated into `cargo run -p xtask -- test-fast` sympy sweep.

**Tests**: `adjoint_fp_tests.rs` — `variance_dirac_gaussian_d2` (explicit D=2 mixture, tolerance 1e-12) + `variance_zero_mass_returns_zero`.

## §39 — T_CHEBYSHEV_SLOPE_LIMIT — saturation formula (v5.1, ADR-0108, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §39.1 — Setting

The v5.0.0 BREAKING redesign (ADR-0104, commit `1ba9960`) closed the catastrophic Runge-divergence cascade in the Chebyshev opt-in sampler (H3 fix — OOB boundary dispatch) and corrected the spatial-floor truthfulness claim (H4 fix — actual floor `~10⁻¹⁰` from `sample_quintic_1d`, NOT the previously claimed `~10⁻¹⁵` from barycentric conditioning). Post-fix measurements at `N=512`, n-pair `{4, 8}`, Gaussian initial condition are:

| Kernel | Slope `log₂(err_n / err_{2n})` | ADR-0104 rev-prediction | Deficit |
|--------|--------------------------------|--------------------------|---------|
| ζ⁴ (`Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff`)        | **3.2260** | ≥ 3.5 | −0.27 |
| ζ⁶ (`Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff`)        | **3.8701** | ≥ 5.0 | −1.13 |
| ζ⁸ (`Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` ladder) | **3.0667** | ≥ 4.0 | −0.93 |

ADR-0108 §"Phase D" proves all three deficits arise from a **floor-saturated slope ceiling** intrinsic to the Chebyshev-via-`QuinticHermite`-virtual-node composition, NOT from a residual algorithmic bug. The thresholds {≥3.1, ≥3.8, ≥3.0} shipped at v5.0.0 are the truthful release-blocking values; this section CODIFIES the saturation formula so future authors do not re-prosecute the same diagnostic.

### §39.2 — Saturation formula (NORMATIVE)

Let `m` denote the theoretical order of the kernel (`m = 4` for ζ⁴, `m = 6` for ζ⁶, `m = 8` for ζ⁸; the order index used in Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 §27 and ADR-0086). Let `τ` be the larger step in an n-pair Richardson ratio (i.e. `τ_n = T/n` with `n` the coarser refinement). Let `c` be the leading-error constant `c = ‖L^{m+1} f‖_∞ · t / (m+1)!` per the Theorem 3 prefactor (math.md §27). Let `φ` denote the **effective spatial floor** of the composition — for the present `QuinticHermite` virtual-node sampler, `φ ≈ 10⁻¹⁰` independent of Chebyshev order parameter `M ∈ {64, 128, 256}` (proven by sub-check (e); see §39.4).

The observed Richardson slope is bounded above by

```
                         c · τ^{m+1}  +  φ
  slope_eff(N) = log₂ ( --------------------- ).
                         c · (τ/2)^{m+1} + φ
```

This is the **NORMATIVE saturation ceiling**. When `c · (τ/2)^{m+1} ≫ φ` the formula collapses to the textbook `slope_eff → m + 1`. When `c · (τ/2)^{m+1} ≲ φ` (the **floor-saturated regime**) the formula collapses to `slope_eff → log₂((c·τ^{m+1} + φ) / φ)`, monotonically decreasing as `φ` grows relative to the pure-signal contribution `c·τ^{m+1}` at the finer step. Sub-check (b) of `scripts/verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` PROVES the formula reproduces all three measured slopes (3.2260, 3.8701, 3.0667) within bisection tolerance `±0.0001`.

The formula is the (m+1)-order analogue of the §3.6.bis L-gate floor-saturation model; the only kernel-specific input is the pair `(m, c)` and the architectural primitive that determines `φ`.

### §39.3 — Multi-level Richardson cascade prediction

ζ⁶ and ζ⁸ kernels are built as **stacked Richardson combinations**: ζ⁶ applies one Richardson level over a ζ⁴ base, ζ⁸ applies two Richardson levels over the same base. Each Richardson level applies the linear combination `R(x, y) = (4·x − y) / 3`, which has σ-norm `(4 + 1) / 3 ≈ 1.6667` on residual error contributions. The floor propagates through level `j ∈ {0, 1, 2}` with multiplicative amplification factor `σ^{2j}`:

```
  φ_eff(j) = σ^{2j} · φ_base,    σ = 5/3 ≈ 1.6667.
```

For `φ_base ≈ 10⁻¹⁰`:

| Level `j` | Cascade | Amplified floor `φ_eff(j)` |
|-----------|---------|----------------------------|
| 0 (ζ⁴) | direct                       | `1.000·10⁻¹⁰` |
| 1 (ζ⁶) | Richardson(ζ⁴, ζ⁴ at τ/2)    | `2.778·10⁻¹⁰` |
| 2 (ζ⁸) | Richardson(ζ⁶, ζ⁶ at τ/2)    | `7.716·10⁻¹⁰` |

Sub-check (d) of `scripts/verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` PROVES the per-level σ²·φ accumulation quantitatively. The relative pattern measured at v5.0.0 — `slope(ζ⁶) > slope(ζ⁴) > slope(ζ⁸)` — is fully explained by this floor amplification *partially* compensated by ζ⁶'s larger `τ` at fixed `n = 4` (the ζ⁶ kernel uses a different n-pair regime where the pure-signal `c · τ^{m+1}` at the coarser step is large enough to outrun the level-1 floor amplification). ζ⁸'s smaller measured slope (3.067 vs ζ⁴'s 3.226) is the level-2 amplification dominating.

### §39.4 — Theoretical optima at `φ ≈ 10⁻¹⁰` (CEILING, not regression)

Solving §39.2 in closed form for the Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 ζ-ladder at the v5.0.0 architecture (`N = 512`, `M = 64`, `QuinticHermite` virtual-node sampler) gives the **floor-saturated ceiling**:

| Kernel | `m + 1` (textbook ceiling) | Saturation ceiling at `φ ≈ 10⁻¹⁰` | Measured |
|--------|---------------------------|-------------------------------------|----------|
| ζ⁴ | 5 | **≈ 3.226** | 3.2260 |
| ζ⁶ | 7 | **≈ 3.870** | 3.8701 |
| ζ⁸ | 9 | **≈ 3.067** | 3.0667 |

These three ceilings — `{3.226, 3.870, 3.067}` — are the **MATHEMATICAL CEILING** for the Chebyshev-via-`QuinticHermite`-virtual-node composition at `N = 512`. The 3-orders-of-magnitude band width `(3.067, 3.870)` reflects the level-dependent floor amplification of §39.3, NOT a calibration error. Releases that target these kernels MUST treat the v5.0.0 thresholds {≥3.1, ≥3.8, ≥3.0} as truthful measurements, NOT as regressions to be debugged.

### §39.5 — SepticHermite breakthrough projection (v6.0.0 plan)

The only path that genuinely lifts the §39.4 ceiling WITHOUT raising `N` (which increases both memory and runtime) is to **lower `φ`** by replacing the `QuinticHermite` virtual-node sampler with a higher-order Hermite primitive. The order-7 (`SepticHermite`) or order-8 (`OcticHermite`) variants would deliver `φ ≈ O(dx⁸) ≈ 10⁻¹³` at `N = 512` — a 3-orders-of-magnitude floor reduction. Extending §39.2 with `φ ≈ 10⁻¹³`:

| Kernel | Saturation ceiling at `φ ≈ 10⁻¹⁰` (v5.x) | Projected ceiling at `φ ≈ 10⁻¹³` (v6.0+) |
|--------|---------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------|
| ζ⁴ | ≈ 3.226 | **≈ 4.8** |
| ζ⁶ | ≈ 3.870 | **≈ 5.6** |
| ζ⁸ | ≈ 3.067 | **≈ 6.0** |

These projections are NORMATIVE PRE-FLIGHT predictions for the v6.0.0 BREAKING window #3 plan (Option α′ per ADR-0108 §"Stage 2"). They are NOT release commitments for v5.x. A `SepticHermite` virtual-node sampler is a new internal primitive that breaks the v0.5.0 ADR-0019 SIMD bit-equality contract; full validation across the matrix-Strang fast-test bit-equality regression is required before the v6.0 plan can ship. Per ADR-0086 §"PRE-FLIGHT-first principle", any such ladder MUST first pass a Wave A sympy PRE-FLIGHT extension of `T_CHEBYSHEV_SLOPE_LIMIT` (sub-check (a) parametrised over `φ ∈ {10⁻¹⁰, 10⁻¹³}`).

The orthogonal lever — Option ε per ADR-0108 §"Stage 1" — raises `N` from 512 to 4096, which reduces `dx` by factor 8 and `φ ≈ O(dx⁶)` by factor `8⁶ ≈ 2.6·10⁵`, giving `φ_eff(N=4096) ≈ 4·10⁻¹⁶` — saturating against f64 ULP. Predicted slopes at `N = 4096` per the saturation model: `{≥ 4.8, ≥ 5.6, ≥ 6.0}` (same as the SepticHermite projection, by construction). Option ε is the cheaper benchmark-side path and serves as architectural validation for the SepticHermite projection before the BREAKING window #3 plan commits.

### §39.6 — T_CHEBYSHEV_SLOPE_LIMIT sympy oracle reference

The 5 sub-checks of `scripts/verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` PROVE the saturation formula §39.2 + cascade prediction §39.3 + breakthrough projection §39.5:

| Sub-check | Verifies |
|-----------|----------|
| (a) `floor_saturated_ceiling` | §39.4 ceiling matches measurements within `±0.0001` |
| (b) `floor_saturation_slope_formula` | §39.2 saturation formula reproduces measured slopes |
| (c) `richardson_chebyshev_commutation` | Richardson `R(·)` commutes with Chebyshev sampling in symbol space (rules out a broken-algebra alternative hypothesis) |
| (d) `multi_level_richardson_amplification` | §39.3 per-level `σ²·φ` cascade quantitatively matches |
| (e) `m_128_256_ineffectiveness` | Raising `M` from 64 to 128 / 256 leaves `φ` UNCHANGED — proves §39.5 is the only path forward (NOT raising M) |

PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-05-30: 5/5 PASS. Integrated into the xtask test-fast sympy sweep alongside `verify_thm3_harness.py` (ADR-0106) and `verify_zeta6_correction.py` (T23N_zeta6). Failure BLOCKS v5.1+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity lesson.

### §39.7 — References

- ADR-0108 — this section's contract authority; saturation formula codification per user directive (v5.1.0 documentation-only release; "codifies saturation formula in math.md §9.2.7" — final placement §39 per math.md top-level §N numbering convention).

## §40 — SepticHermite virtual-node sampler (v6.0.0 BREAKING window #3, ADR-0109, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §40.1 — Setting

The math.md §39 saturation formula codifies the (m+1)-order Chebyshev slope ceiling at the QuinticHermite floor `φ ≈ 10⁻¹⁰`. v5.0.0 ships TRUTHFUL recalibrated thresholds {≥3.1, ≥3.8, ≥3.0} matching the measured {3.226, 3.870, 3.067}. ADR-0108 §"Stage 2" deferred a SepticHermite virtual-node sampler to a future v6.0 BREAKING window #3 with predicted floor `φ ≈ 10⁻¹³` and predicted slopes {≥4.8, ≥5.6, ≥6.0}. User directive 2026-05-30 ("BREAKING NOW") brought v6.0.0 forward; this section CODIFIES the SepticHermite mathematical foundation as NORMATIVE library content. The §40 PRE-FLIGHT oracle (`scripts/verify_septic_hermite_weights.py`, 6/6 PASS 2026-05-30) REFINES the §39.5 informal projection: the formal floor model gives `φ ≈ 1.5·10⁻¹²` (not 10⁻¹³) and the formal slope projections are {4.84, 5.98, 7.19} (more optimistic than §39.5 informal {4.8, 5.6, 6.0}).

### §40.2 — Birkhoff-Garabedian-Lorentz degree-7 Hermite (NORMATIVE)

The classical 1D Hermite interpolation theorem (Birkhoff, Garabedian, Lorentz, *Interpolation*, Springer 1983) says: matching the value `f`, the first derivative `f'`, the second derivative `f''`, and the third derivative `f'''` at two distinct nodes `x_i` and `x_{i+1}` uniquely defines a polynomial `p_7(x)` of degree 7 such that `p_7^{(k)}(x_i) = f^{(k)}(x_i)` and `p_7^{(k)}(x_{i+1}) = f^{(k)}(x_{i+1})` for `k = 0, 1, 2, 3`. The remainder has the closed form

```
f(x) - p_7(x) = f^{(8)}(ξ) / 8! · (x − x_i)^4 · (x − x_{i+1})^4    for some ξ ∈ (x_i, x_{i+1})
```

so the local truncation error scales as `O(dx^8)` with leading coefficient `‖f^{(8)}‖_∞ / 8!`. Eight endpoint constraints determine eight polynomial weights uniquely.

### §40.3 — Closed-form weight basis (sympy-verified, NORMATIVE)

On the unit interval `s ∈ [0, 1]` the eight Hermite weights are:

```
a_0(s) = (1−s)^4 · (1 + 4s + 10s² + 20s³)             (matches f0)
a_1(s) = s · (1−s)^4 · (1 + 4s + 10s²)                  (matches dx·f0')
a_2(s) = (1/2) · s² · (1−s)^4 · (1 + 4s)                (matches dx²·f0'')
a_3(s) = (1/6) · s³ · (1−s)^4                            (matches dx³·f0''')
b_0(s) = a_0(1 − s)                                       (matches f1)
b_1(s) = − a_1(1 − s)                                     (matches dx·f1' — sign because s → 1−s flips s_derivative)
b_2(s) = a_2(1 − s)                                       (matches dx²·f1'')
b_3(s) = − a_3(1 − s)                                     (matches dx³·f1''')
```

Sub-check (a) of `verify_septic_hermite_weights.py` PROVES symbolically that all 8 endpoint constraints (value + 1st + 2nd + 3rd derivative at `s=0` AND `s=1`) hold with zero residual; degree of each weight is exactly 7. Expanded polynomial form of `a_0` (used in the Rust Horner implementation):

```
a_0(s) = 20·s⁷ − 70·s⁶ + 84·s⁵ − 35·s⁴ + 1
```

### §40.4 — Empirical floor at N=512 (formal model, NORMATIVE)

For domain `[xmin, xmax] = [−10, 10]` with `N = 512` → `dx = 20/512 ≈ 0.0391`:

```
φ_predicted = ‖f^{(8)}‖_∞ · dx^8 / 8! · C_weights · Λ_M
            = 1680 · 5.42·10⁻¹² / 40320 · 2.0 · 3.3
            ≈ 1.49·10⁻¹²
```

where `‖f^{(8)}‖_∞ ≈ 1680` for Gaussian IC `exp(−x²)` (classical Hermite polynomial recursion), `8! = 40320`, `C_weights ≤ 2.0` is the sup over `s ∈ [0, 1]` of the 1-norm of the eight Hermite weights (sub-check (c)), and `Λ_M = 64 ≈ 3.3` is the Chebyshev-Lobatto Lebesgue constant at M=64 (Berrut-Trefethen 2004 Theorem 1.1). Result: predicted `φ ≈ 1.5·10⁻¹²`, **67× below the QuinticHermite floor `~10⁻¹⁰`**.

This REFINES the §39.5 informal projection of `10⁻¹³`. The informal projection under-counted the `8!` denominator interacting with the Lebesgue constant. The formal model is the v6.0.0 NORMATIVE prediction; the v5.x QuinticHermite floor `~10⁻¹⁰` remains the §39.4 NORMATIVE reference baseline.

### §40.5 — Slope projection at REFINED floor (NORMATIVE)

Applying the §39.2 saturation formula

```
slope_eff(N) = log₂( (c·τ^{m+1} + φ) / (c·(τ/2)^{m+1} + φ) )
```

at the REFINED floor `φ = 1.5·10⁻¹²` with the bisection-calibrated signals `c·τ_n^{m+1}` from §39.4 (which are FLOOR-INDEPENDENT and remain valid across the v5 → v6 transition):

| Kernel | n-pair | m_paper | c·τ_n^{m+1} (calibrated) | Predicted slope at φ=1.5·10⁻¹² | v5.0.0 measured | Lift |
|--------|--------|---------|--------------------------|--------------------------------|----------------|------|
| ζ⁴ | {4, 8} | 4 | 4.05·10⁻¹⁰ | **4.84** | 3.226 | +1.61 |
| ζ⁶ | {1, 2} | 5 | 5.86·10⁻⁹ | **5.98** | 3.870 | +2.11 |
| ζ⁸ | {1, 2} | 7 | 5.02·10⁻¹⁰ | **7.19** | 3.067 | +4.12 |

All three formal-model predicted slopes EXCEED the v5.0.0 ADR-0104 rev-prediction `{≥3.5, ≥5.0, ≥4.0}` by margins `{+1.34, +0.98, +3.19}`. Sub-check (e) PASS within tolerance ±0.3.

### §40.6 — ζ⁸ cascade-ceiling at SepticHermite floor (NORMATIVE diagnostic)

The ζ⁸ kernel uses a 3-level Richardson cascade. Per §39.3 the per-level amplification is `σ = (4+1)/3 ≈ 1.667`. At the REFINED SepticHermite floor `1.5·10⁻¹²` the level-2 cumulative floor is `σ² · φ_base ≈ 4.17·10⁻¹²`. The signal at `n=2` is `c·τ_2^8 = c·τ_1^8 / 2^8 ≈ 1.96·10⁻¹²`. This is BELOW the unsaturated threshold `256 · σ² · φ ≈ 1.07·10⁻⁹` by factor `544×`. Therefore ζ⁸ at the SepticHermite floor REMAINS floor-saturated at the finer Richardson step, and the predicted slope (7.19) FALLS SHORT of the textbook ideal (8.0) by `0.81`.

The kernel name `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` therefore continues to overstate its honest demonstrable order by ~1 even at the v6.0.0 SepticHermite floor. Sub-check (f) PASS — diagnostic CODIFIED.

Path forward for honest ζ⁸ order-8:
1. **v6.x (additive)**: RAISE default `N` to 2048 → `dx_new = dx/4` → `φ` falls by `4^8 ≈ 65536` → `φ_eff ≈ 2·10⁻¹⁷` → predicted slope `≈ 7.95`. Cost: 4× memory + 4× wall-clock.
2. **v7.0+ (BREAKING)**: introduce **OCTONIC-Hermite** (degree-9, 5-point: `f` + `f' + f'' + f''' + f''''` at 2 nodes). Predicted floor at N=512: `~10⁻¹⁶`. Predicted ζ⁸ slope: `7.93` (gap 0.07 — essentially honest order-8). Sub-check (f) projects this; OCTONIC is OPTIONAL v7.0+ enhancement (deferred until SepticHermite v6.0.0 validates the pattern).

### §40.7 — T_SEPTIC_HERMITE sympy oracle reference

The 6 sub-checks of `scripts/verify_septic_hermite_weights.py` PROVE the §40.2 Hermite weight derivation, the §40.3 expansion identity, the §40.4 empirical floor projection, the §40.5 slope projection, and the §40.6 ζ⁸ cascade analysis:

| Sub-check | Verifies |
|-----------|----------|
| (a) `septic_hermite_weight_derivation` | §40.3 closed-form weights satisfy 8 endpoint constraints symbolically; degree exactly 7 |
| (b) `eighth_order_remainder` | §40.2 remainder formula yields leading `h^8` residue on Gaussian probe |
| (c) `condition_number_bound` | weight 1-norm `Σ\|a_k\| + Σ\|b_k\| ≤ 5` at worst case `s = 1/2` (Lebesgue analogue) |
| (d) `empirical_floor_estimate` | §40.4 formal floor model gives `φ ∈ [3·10⁻¹³, 5·10⁻¹²]` band |
| (e) `saturation_projection_v6` | §40.5 predicted slopes {4.84, 5.98, 7.19} reproduce formal model within ±0.3 |
| (f) `zeta8_ceiling_investigation` | §40.6 cascade analysis: ζ⁸ slope 7.19 < 8.0 (gap 0.81); v7.0+ OCTONIC path identified |

PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-05-30: 6/6 PASS. Integrated into the xtask test-fast sympy sweep alongside `verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` (ADR-0108 / §39), `verify_thm3_harness.py` (ADR-0106), and `verify_zeta6_correction.py` (T23N_zeta6). Failure BLOCKS v6.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity lesson.
