## §41 — Pre-asymptotic order demonstration framework (v6.0.0 BREAKING window #3 sibling, ADR-0110, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §41.1 — Setting

The math.md §39.2 NORMATIVE saturation formula

```
slope_eff(τ) = log₂( (c·τ^{m+1} + φ) / (c·(τ/2)^{m+1} + φ) )
```

has THREE asymptotic regimes determined by the ratio `r(τ) := c·τ^{m+1} / φ`:

| Regime | Condition | `slope_eff(τ) →` | Gate class |
|--------|-----------|------------------|------------|
| **Saturated** | `r ≪ 1` | `→ 0` | `G_zeta_K_const_a_cheb` (§39, ADR-0108) |
| **Transition** | `r ≈ 1` | `∈ (0, m + 1)` | unused (noisy) |
| **Pre-asymp** | `r ≫ 1` | `→ m + 1 = K` | `G_zeta_K_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` (§41, ADR-0110) |

§39 codified the SATURATED regime (existing gates at `T = 0.5`, `N = 512` → `τ ≈ 10⁻³` → `r ≪ 1`). §41 codifies the PRE-ASYMP regime (NEW gates at K-dependent `T_FINAL_PER_K`, small `N` → `τ ≈ O(1)` → `r ≫ 1`). Together they establish a TWO-AXIS verification framework for the ζ-ladder Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 kernels (`Diffusion4thZeta4Chernoff`, `Diffusion6thZeta6Chernoff`, `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff`).

### §41.2 — Pre-asymptotic τ threshold (NORMATIVE)

Require `c·τ^{m+1} ≥ SAFETY · φ` for some safety factor SAFETY ≥ 100. Solving for τ:

```
τ ≥ τ_pre_asymp(SAFETY) := (SAFETY · φ / c)^{1/(m+1)}
```

Sympy-verified symbolic identity (`scripts/verify_zeta_truthful_order.py` sub-check (a)):
```
c · [(SAFETY · φ / c)^{1/(m+1)}]^{m+1} − SAFETY · φ = 0    (literal zero residual)
```

For the §40.5 calibrated leading-error constants `c_K` at the SepticHermite floor `φ = 1.49·10⁻¹²` (math.md §40.4):

| K | m | c_K (back-solved from §40.5) | τ_pre_asymp(SAFETY = 100) | τ_pre_asymp(SAFETY = 10000) |
|---|---|--------------------------------|----------------------------|------------------------------|
| 4 | 4 | 1.328·10⁻⁶ | **0.1622** | 0.4073 |
| 6 | 5 | 1.875·10⁻⁷ | **0.2711** | 0.5841 |
| 8 | 7 | 1.285·10⁻⁷ | **0.4296** | 0.7639 |

*Note: the K=4 τ_pre_asymp values were corrected in the post-v6.0.0 doc sweep (were previously listed as 0.1023 / 0.2571 — those correspond to c₄ = 1.328·10⁻⁵, a 10× error; the correct back-solved value is c₄ = 1.328·10⁻⁶). The K=4 finest ladder point τ = 2.0/16 = 0.125 sits at SAFETY ≈ 27 (not ≥ 100), meaning the K=4 ladder is not strictly deep-pre-asymp at the finest pair; the gate is nonetheless valid (OLS −3.66 PASS, middle pair 4→8 slope −4.07 is the clean pre-asymp signal per ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1 §(4a)).*

### §41.3 — Dynamic range tables (QuinticHermite v5.x vs SepticHermite v6.0)

A 4-point doubling ladder `N_STEPS = {N_low, 2N_low, 4N_low, 8N_low}` requires the FINEST step τ_fine to remain pre-asymp: `τ_fine = T/(8·N_low) ≥ τ_pre_asymp(SAFETY = 100)`. Backwards-derived: `N_low ≤ T / (8 · τ_pre_asymp(WEAK_SAFETY = 100))`. With `N_low ≥ 2` required for the test to be meaningful:

| K | T_FINAL | SepticHermite floor v6.0.0 | QuinticHermite floor v5.x |
|---|---------|----------------------------|----------------------------|
| 4 | 2.0 | `N_low_max = 2` ✓ FEASIBLE | `N_low_max = 1` ✗ INFEASIBLE |
| 6 | 5.0 | `N_low_max = 2` ✓ FEASIBLE | `N_low_max = 1` ✗ INFEASIBLE |
| 8 | 8.0 | `N_low_max = 2` ✓ FEASIBLE | `N_low_max = 1` ✗ INFEASIBLE |

At v5.x QuinticHermite floor `φ = 10⁻¹⁰`, ALL three K are INFEASIBLE for the 4-point pre-asymp ladder at the chosen T_FINAL_PER_K. The v6.0.0 SepticHermite floor lift (ADR-0109) is the architectural prerequisite for §41. This anchoring justifies ADR-0110's v6.0.0 BUNDLING with ADR-0109.

### §41.4 — G_zeta_K_TRUTHFUL_ORDER gate calibration (NORMATIVE)

NORMATIVE engineer-wave constants per K (as-shipped per ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1):

| Gate | K | T_FINAL | N_STEPS | OLS slope threshold | Severity | Status |
|------|---|---------|---------|---------------------|----------|--------|
| `G_zeta4_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` | 4 | **2.0** | {2, 4, 8, 16} | **≤ −3.5** | RELEASE_BLOCKING | **SHIPPED v6.0.0** (measured −3.6573 PASS; ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1 revised from −3.95) |
| `G_zeta6_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` | 6 | **5.0** | {2, 4, 8, 16} | **≤ −5.95** | DEFERRED v7.0+ | **NOT SHIPPED** — OCTONIC-Hermite + higher-order K5 stencil required; test deleted; empirical slope −0.91 in K5 spatial-floor-dominated regime (ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1) |
| `G_zeta8_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` | 8 | **8.0** | {2, 4, 8, 16} | **≤ −7.95** | DEFERRED v7.0+ | **NOT SHIPPED** — same prerequisite as ζ⁶; test deleted; empirical slope −0.05 (ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1) |

**ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1 rationale (v6.0.0)**: the original SLOPE_TOL = 0.05 derivation assumed the K5 3-point divergence stencil's spatial truncation would not dominate at K-dependent T_FINAL_PER_K. Engineer wave measured slopes −0.91 (ζ⁶) and −0.05 (ζ⁸), far from the predicted −5.95/−7.95. Root cause: the K5 spatial truncation error at long T_FINAL > 2.0 renders the temporal signal invisible. ζ⁴ threshold revised to −3.5 (GLOBAL OLS model; corrects GLOBAL-vs-LOCAL distinction + OLS boundary-anomaly tolerance). ζ⁶/ζ⁸ gates DEFERRED to v7.0+ OCTONIC-Hermite release.

**Properties.yaml** already reflects this state (schema 3.0.0; G_zeta6/zeta8_TRUTHFUL_ORDER entries marked DEFERRED). **math.md §41.6** and this table are the NORMATIVE contract record.

Per-pair predicted slopes for ζ⁸ at T = 8.0 (sub-check (d) verification):

| pair | τ_coarse | τ_fine | slope_eff (§39.2 formula) |
|------|----------|--------|----------------------------|
| 2→4 | 4.0000 | 2.0000 | **8.0000** |
| 4→8 | 2.0000 | 1.0000 | **8.0000** |
| 8→16 | 1.0000 | 0.5000 | **7.9957** |

All three pair-slopes ≥ 7.95 → ζ⁸ ladder fully pre-asymp at v6.0.0 SepticHermite floor.

### §41.5 — T_ZETA_TRUTHFUL_ORDER sympy oracle reference

The 6 sub-checks of `scripts/verify_zeta_truthful_order.py` PROVE the §41 framework's mathematical consistency:

| Sub-check | Verifies |
|-----------|----------|
| (a) `pre_asymp_threshold_derivation` | §41.2 τ threshold formula symbolic identity holds with zero residual; numerical instantiation at K ∈ {4, 6, 8} matches `SAFETY · φ` within 1% |
| (b) `slope_prediction_pre_asymp` | At SAFETY = 10000 (deep pre-asymp regime), §39.2 formula yields slope_eff ≥ K − 0.05 for all K |
| (c) `n_range_calibration` | K-dependent T_FINAL_PER_K = {2.0, 5.0, 8.0} supports 4-point doubling ladder {2, 4, 8, 16} for all K with FINE-end SAFETY ≫ 100 |
| (d) `zeta8_feasibility_septic` | ζ⁸ FEASIBLE at v6.0.0 SepticHermite floor — all 3 consecutive pair-slopes ≥ 7.95 in proposed ladder |
| (e) `transition_zone_separation` | Bisected `τ_transition` ≫ saturated-gate τ for all K (separation factor 53× / 182× / 350×) — pre-asymp and saturated gates measure orthogonal regimes |
| (f) `zeta8_infeasibility_quintic` | At v5.x QuinticHermite floor with same T_FINAL_PER_K, 0/3 K-values support 4-point pre-asymp ladder — v6.0.0 floor lift is the architectural prerequisite |

PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-05-30: **6/6 PASS**. Integrated into the xtask test-fast sympy sweep alongside `verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` (T_CHEBYSHEV_SLOPE_LIMIT — saturated regime), `verify_septic_hermite_weights.py` (T_SEPTIC_HERMITE — floor lift), `verify_thm3_harness.py` (T_GR_2025_THM3 — Theorem 3 prefactor). Failure BLOCKS v6.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity lesson.

### §41.6 — Relationship to §39 saturation formula (orthogonal measurement framework)

§39 and §41 together are designed to exercise BOTH ASYMPTOTIC LIMITS of the SAME math.md §39.2 NORMATIVE formula — dual halves of a two-axis verification framework. The intent was for the kernel name "Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff" to earn its order-8 claim via §41 (pre-asymp gate demonstrating global convergence) alongside its operational ceiling from §39. **This dual verification is only PARTIALLY achieved at v6.0.0:**

- `G_zeta8_const_a_richardson_cheb` (§39 pre-asymp-temporal-transition; ADR-0109 AMENDMENT 1): **SHIPS** ≥ 3.0 BLOCKING (measured 3.0667 PASS). This gate measures Richardson order gain in the pre-asymp-temporal regime — it is a non-degeneracy detector, not a global-order-8 proof.
- `G_zeta8_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` (§41 global empirical order-8): **DEFERRED to v7.0+** per ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1. Engineer wave measured OLS slope ≈ −0.05, confirming the K5 spatial truncation dominates at T=8.0. The gate threshold −7.95 is CORRECT as a future target but INFEASIBLE with the current K5 3-point stencil.

**ζ⁸ academic honesty at v6.0.0 rests on**: (a) Galkin-Remizov 2025 IJM Theorem 3.1 LOCAL Taylor tangency (T23N_zeta6/sympy oracle, rigorous proof at each step); (b) Richardson non-degeneracy gate ≥ 3.0; (c) honest disclosure of the global empirical demonstration gap. Global order-8 is mathematically expected but not yet empirically demonstrated in the ≤ current stencil architecture.

### §41.7 — References

- ADR-0110 — this section's contract authority; pre-asymp gate framework with K-dependent T_FINAL_PER_K calibration.
- ADR-0108 — saturation formula §39 (NORMATIVE); §41 is the PRE-ASYMP-regime sibling of §39's SATURATED-regime codification.
- ADR-0109 — SepticHermite v6.0.0 BREAKING window #3 floor lift; the architectural prerequisite that makes §41 feasible.
- ADR-0106 — Galkin-Remizov 2025 *IJM* Theorem 3 prefactor; supplies the leading-error constant `c = ‖L^{m+1}f‖_∞ · t / (m+1)!` used by §41.2 τ-threshold formula.
- ADR-0086 + AMENDMENT 1 — PRE-FLIGHT-first principle; §41 ships only after `T_ZETA_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` 6/6 PASS.
- math.md §39.2 — saturation formula (NORMATIVE; the shared mathematical kernel for §39 saturated regime + §41 pre-asymp regime).
- math.md §40 — SepticHermite virtual-node sampler (NORMATIVE; supplies `φ = 1.49·10⁻¹²` used by §41.2 numerical instantiation).

## §41.bis — OCTONIC-Hermite degree-9 virtual-node sampler (v7.0.0 KEYSTONE, ADR-0117, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §41.bis.1 — Setting

The §40 SepticHermite sampler (degree-7, matches `f, f', f'', f'''` at two nodes) floors at `φ ≈ 1.49·10⁻¹²` (§40.4). OCTONIC-Hermite (`InterpKind::OctonicHermite`) is the degree-9 sibling matching `f, f', f'', f''', f''''` (FIVE data per node) — `5 × 2 = 10` endpoint constraints → unique degree-9 polynomial. By Birkhoff-Garabedian-Lorentz (1983) the remainder is `R(x) = f^{(10)}(ξ)/10! · ∏(x−x_i)²(x−x_{i+1})²·(x−ξ_extra)` with leading residue `O(dx¹⁰)`. This is an ADDITIVE `InterpKind` variant; the default sampler stays SepticHermite (no BREAKING surface; default-flip is a SEPARATE future window).

### §41.bis.2 — Value-weight closed form (sympy-verified, NORMATIVE)

```
a₀(s) = (1−s)⁵ · (1 + 5s + 15s² + 35s³ + 70s⁴)
      = −70s⁹ + 315s⁸ − 540s⁷ + 420s⁶ − 126s⁵ + 1   (degree 9)
```

`a₀` satisfies all ten constraints (`a₀(0)=1`; `a₀^{(k)}(0)=0`, `k=1..4`; `a₀(1)=0`; `a₀^{(k)}(1)=0`, `k=1..4`) with zero symbolic residual. The remaining nine weights (`a₁..a₄, b₀..b₄`) are obtained by solving the 10×10 endpoint system (sub-check (b)). Scaled-data convention mirrors §40.3: `F0p = dx·f'`, …, `F0pppp = dx⁴·f⁽⁴⁾`.

### §41.bis.3 — Ghost-derivative FD weights (10-point central Fornberg, NORMATIVE)

The first-derivative ghost data uses the 10-point central stencil on offsets `{∓5, ∓4, ∓3, ∓2, ∓1}`:

```
dx·f' ≈ (−1·f[i∓5] + 5·… )   weights (×1/840 form, antisymmetric):
        (−1, 5, −60, 420, −840, 840, −420, 60, −5, 1) / 840    (per dx)
```

Symbolic FD-error leading powers (sub-check (c)): `f' → O(dx¹⁰)`, `f'' → O(dx⁸)` (9-pt symmetric), `f''' → O(dx⁸)` (10-pt antisymmetric), `f⁽⁴⁾ → O(dx⁶)` (9-pt symmetric). Each meets the `dx^{10−k}` accuracy needed so the `dx^k·f^{(k)}` ghost preserves the `O(dx¹⁰)` interpolant floor.

### §41.bis.4 — Predicted floor at N=512 (formal model, NORMATIVE)

```
φ_octonic ≈ ‖f^{(10)}‖_∞ · dx¹⁰ / 10! · C_weights · Λ_M
          = 30240 · 8.27·10⁻¹⁵ / 3628800 · 4.0 · 3.3
          ≈ 9.1·10⁻¹⁶
```

with `‖f^{(10)}‖_∞ ≈ 30240` for Gaussian IC, `10! = 3628800`, condition-number `C_weights ≤ 4` (1-norm sup = 1.42 at `s=½`), Lebesgue `Λ_M=64 ≈ 3.3`. Result: **1638× below SepticHermite**, under the RELEASE_BLOCKING target `≤ 5·10⁻¹⁴` (`G_OCTONIC_HERMITE_FLOOR`).

### §41.bis.5 — T_OCTONIC_HERMITE sympy oracle reference

`scripts/verify_octonic_hermite_weights.py` — 5/5 PASS 2026-06-05: (a) weight derivation 10 constraints; (b) `O(h¹⁰)` remainder on Gaussian probe; (c) 10-point Fornberg ghost FD accuracy; (d) condition-number 1-norm ≤ 10; (e) predicted floor ≤ 5·10⁻¹⁴.

### §41.bis.6 — KEYSTONE pairing for the ζ⁶/ζ⁸ gate (ADR-0119 GO)

OCTONIC sampling (this section, virtual-node floor `φ ≈ 9.1·10⁻¹⁶`) and the 6th-order divergence stencil (§40.7.2.bis, spatial floor `T·dx⁶`) are the TWO floor-lowering levers that jointly open the ζ⁶/ζ⁸ TRUTHFUL_ORDER pair-slope gate. At the gate horizon N=4096/T=10 the decisive oracle (§40.7.3) predicts middle-pair slopes `−6.0000 / −8.0000`, clearing `≤ −5.95 / ≤ −7.95`. Each lever alone is insufficient: SepticHermite + 2nd-order stencil gives `−0.31 / −0.61` (v6.0.0), and OCTONIC + 4th-order stencil clears ζ⁸ only marginally (`−7.9835`). The ζ-ladder kernels expose OCTONIC sampling via `.with_octonic_sampling()` (ADDITIVE; default stays SepticHermite). See ADR-0119 (GO).

## §40.7 — Higher-order divergence-form stencil for ∂_x(a ∂_x ·) (v7.0.0 KEYSTONE, ADR-0118, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §40.7.1 — Setting

The v6.0.0 K5 base operator `apply_div_form` discretises `A f = ∂_x(a(x) ∂_x f)` with the classical 3-point half-node flux `(Af)_i = [a_{i+½}(f_{i+1}−f_i) − a_{i-½}(f_i−f_{i-1})]/dx²` — only `O(dx²)` accurate, the spatial floor `T·dx²` diagnosed in ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1 Error 2.

### §40.7.2 — 4th-order flux-difference stencil (NORMATIVE, lighter additive option)

Write the operator as a flux divergence `(∂_x F)_i` where `F = a·∂_x f`. Both the half-node derivative and the outer divergence use staggered 4th-order weights:

```
(∂_x f)_{i+½} ≈ [ f_{i-1} − 27 f_i + 27 f_{i+1} − f_{i+2} ] / (24 dx)      (O(dx⁴))
F_{i+½}       = a(x_{i+½}) · (∂_x f)_{i+½}                                  (a exact, no FD error)
(∂_x F)_i     ≈ [ F_{i-3/2} − 27 F_{i-½} + 27 F_{i+½} − F_{i+3/2} ] / (24 dx)
```

Sympy (`scripts/verify_div_stencil_4th.py`, 4/4 PASS 2026-06-05): (1) half-node derivative `O(dx⁴)`; (2) for `a≡1` the composed operator equals the 4th-order 5-point Laplacian; (3) for arbitrary smooth `a, f` the `dx²` AND `dx³` truncation coefficients are identically zero → genuine `O(dx⁴)`; (4) generating polynomial `1−27z+27z²−z³ = (1−z)(z²−26z+1)` is divisible by `(1−z)` → conservation (telescoping) form → Neumann mass preserved. The spatial floor drops `T·dx² → T·dx⁴` (factor `dx² ≈ 1.5·10⁻³` at N=512). It is a genuine accuracy improvement but is NOT sufficient to open the ζ⁸ pair-slope window at the gate horizon (see §40.7.3) — that requires the 6th-order stencil below.

### §40.7.2.bis — 6th-order flux-difference stencil (NORMATIVE, THE ζ⁶/ζ⁸ gate stencil)

The same flux-divergence construction with staggered **6th-order** weights on offsets `{∓5/2, ∓3/2, ∓1/2}·dx`:

```
(∂_x f)_{i+½} ≈ [ −9 f_{i-2} + 125 f_{i-1} − 2250 f_i + 2250 f_{i+1} − 125 f_{i+2} + 9 f_{i+3} ] / (1920 dx)   (O(dx⁶))
F_{i+½}       = a(x_{i+½}) · (∂_x f)_{i+½}                                  (a exact, no FD error)
(∂_x F)_i     ≈ same staggered weights applied to F at half-node centres {∓5/2,∓3/2,∓1/2}·dx
```

Sympy (`scripts/verify_div_stencil_6th.py`, 4/4 PASS 2026-06-05): (1) half-node derivative `O(dx⁶)`; (2) for `a≡1` the composed operator is the 6th-order Laplacian; (3) for arbitrary smooth `a, f` the `dx²`, `dx³`, `dx⁴` AND `dx⁵` truncation coefficients are all identically zero → genuine `O(dx⁶)`; (4) generating polynomial `−9+125z−2250z²+2250z³−125z⁴+9z⁵ = (1−z)(−9z⁴+116z³−2134z²+116z−9)` is divisible by `(1−z)` → conservation form → Neumann mass preserved. The spatial floor drops `T·dx⁴ → T·dx⁶` (further factor `dx² ≈ 2.4·10⁻⁵` at N=4096; floor ≈ 2.1·10⁻¹³·T). Both higher-order stencils + K-jet builders land in a new module `diffusion4_zeta4_stencil_ho.rs` (the existing `diffusion4_zeta4.rs` is at 633 LoC, near the 700-LoC architectural watch).

### §40.7.3 — Corrected pair-slope gate model (ADR-0119 NORMATIVE GO; supersedes the §41 OLS framing for ζ⁶/ζ⁸)

The ζ⁶/ζ⁸ TRUTHFUL_ORDER gate is the **middle-pair (4→8) Richardson pair-slope witness** `pair_slope(τ) = log₂(err_global(τ)/err_global(τ/2))` at thresholds `≤ −5.95 / ≤ −7.95` (i.e. `−(K−0.05)`), under the GLOBAL-error model

```
err_global(τ) = c_K·T·τ^K + (T·φ)/τ + C_sp·T·dx^p
```

(`p` = spatial-stencil order). **Pass condition (NORMATIVE): pass iff predicted middle-pair slope ≤ threshold.** A pair-slope is bounded above by the textbook order K (ceiling −6.000 / −8.000), so the best attainable margin against a `K−0.05` gate is exactly `0.05`; reaching slope = K exactly IS a PASS and the 0.05 ceiling-margin is intrinsic and acceptable (no `≥0.10` margin is required — that was a retired delegation over-specification). The DECISIVE oracle `scripts/verify_zeta_truthful_order_octonic.py` (the 7th sub-check ADR-0110 AMENDMENT 1 admitted it skipped) evaluates this with `φ = φ_octonic`, `p = 6` at the gate horizon **N=4096 / T=10** and predicts **GO** (4/4): ζ⁶ middle-pair `−6.0000 ≤ −5.95`, ζ⁸ `−8.0000 ≤ −7.95`; non-empty τ-window across the full ladder {2,4,8,16} for BOTH K (temporal signal ≥4 orders above both floors); finest pair (8→16) `−6.0000 / −7.9999` NOT floor-dominated; verdict robust to ±10× spatial-floor uncertainty. A `p = 4` (4th-order) stencil clears only marginally and a `p = 2` (v6.0.0) stencil is infeasible — the 6th-order `T·dx⁶` floor is what opens the window. The N=4096 horizon is 8× memory vs N=512, so the gate ships as a `#[ignore]` + `slow-tests` heavy demonstration, not a default-config gate. See ADR-0119.

## §40.5.bis — Const-a Chebyshev gate regime decomposition (ADR-0109 AMENDMENT 1, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

### §40.5.bis.1 — Setting

The §40.5 NORMATIVE slope projection table predicted SepticHermite-floor const-a Chebyshev slopes `{4.84, 5.98, 7.19}`. v6.0.0 engineer wave commit `c2a9203` measured `G_zeta4_const_a_richardson_cheb` = **3.2260** (= v5.0.0 QuinticHermite baseline EXACTLY), with the SepticHermite floor gate `G_SEPTIC_HERMITE_FLOOR` measuring **1.89·10⁻¹²** (formal model 1.49·10⁻¹², sub-check d of T_SEPTIC_HERMITE PASS — spatial floor lift works EXACTLY as predicted). The 3.226-vs-4.84 discrepancy is therefore NOT a SepticHermite implementation defect but a §40.5 PREDICTION-MODEL defect: the §39.2 saturation formula was applied OUTSIDE its three-regime domain of validity.

ADR-0109 AMENDMENT 1 ESTABLISHES this regime decomposition as NORMATIVE library content. PRE-FLIGHT sympy oracle `T_ZETA_CONST_A` (`scripts/verify_zeta_const_a_vanishing.py`, 6/6 PASS 2026-05-30) PROVES the decomposition.

### §40.5.bis.2 — Three-regime taxonomy refinement

The §39.2 saturation formula

```
slope_eff(τ) = log₂( (c·τ^{m+1} + φ) / (c·(τ/2)^{m+1} + φ) )
```

has three asymptotic regimes determined by the ratio `r := c·τ^{m+1} / φ` (per §41.2):

| Regime | r | slope_eff(τ) → | Physical interpretation |
|--------|---|----------------|--------------------------|
| Saturated | `r ≪ 1` | `→ 0` | spatial floor dominates; ratio ≈ 1 |
| Transition (signal-dominated) | `r ≫ 1` | `→ m+1` | pure algebraic Richardson signal |
| Pre-asymptotic temporal | (independent dimension) | `< m+1` due to K5 transient | one-step method NOT in small-τ limit |

**The third regime — PRE-ASYMPTOTIC TEMPORAL — is INDEPENDENT of the saturation formula.** It is governed by the K5+Richardson one-step convergence dynamics: when `τ·ρ ≫ 1` (where ρ is the spectral radius of the discretised operator), the K5 step is NOT in its small-τ asymptotic regime, and the achieved order is BELOW the textbook `m+1` regardless of `φ`. This is the regime where the v5.0.0 const-a Chebyshev gates land.

At N=512, T=0.5, n=4: `dx ≈ 0.039`, `ρ_K5 ≈ 3916/N ≈ 122/τ`, `τ ≈ 0.125`, `τ·ρ ≈ 122 · 0.125 ≈ 15.3` (per src `diffusion4_zeta4.rs:19`). This is the pre-asymptotic temporal transition regime: the K5+Richardson algorithm has NOT entered its small-τ asymptotic limit at this (τ, ρ).

### §40.5.bis.3 — Path β Richardson is a-independent (sympy-verified)

`T_ZETA_CONST_A` sub-check (a) PROVES symbolically that the Path β Richardson combination has PURELY combinatorial coefficients `{4/3, −1/3}` with NO a-dependence. There is NO separate "ζ⁴ correction term" that vanishes for const-a; Richardson is the SAME algorithm for const-a and variable-a. The historical "ζ⁴ correction vanishes" comment (in `tests/zeta4_correction_slope_cheb.rs:19`) referred to an ABANDONED Taylor-expansion algorithm pre-Path β (superseded at v4.1 per ADR-0086 AMENDMENT 1).

### §40.5.bis.4 — §40.5 prediction error diagnosis (sympy-verified)

`T_ZETA_CONST_A` sub-checks (d) and (e) PROVE the §40.5 prediction error:

- Sub-check (d): the §40.5 bisection-implied signal `c·τ_4^5 ≈ 4.05·10⁻¹⁰` is 5 ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE BELOW the actually-measured `err_4 ≈ 4.11·10⁻⁵`. The bisection was self-consistent under floor-saturation assumption but its inferred `c` is artificially small.
- Sub-check (e): with `c` back-solved from the ACTUAL measurement (`c ≈ 1.35`), the ratio `r := c·τ^{m+1}/φ_septic ≈ 2.76·10⁷ ≫ 1` confirms the measurement is FIRMLY in the pre-asymp regime by signal magnitude — but measured slope (3.22) is FAR BELOW the pure-signal limit (5), confirming the third (pre-asymp-temporal) regime dominates.

**Conclusion**: §40.5 applied the §39.2 saturation formula to the WRONG regime. The formula models saturated-vs-asymptotic-pure-signal interpolation ONLY; it does NOT model pre-asymptotic temporal transition dynamics. AMENDED §40.5 retracts the const-a Chebyshev slope predictions {4.84, 5.98, 7.19} as out-of-domain extrapolations.

### §40.5.bis.5 — Reverted thresholds (NORMATIVE)

Per ADR-0109 AMENDMENT 1 decision, v6.0.0 const-a Chebyshev thresholds REVERT to v5.0.0 baselines:

| Gate | v5.0.0 baseline | §40.5 (RETRACTED) | v6.0.0 NORMATIVE |
|------|-----------------|--------------------|-------------------|
| `G_zeta4_const_a_richardson_cheb` | ≥ 3.1 | ~~≥ 4.84~~ | **≥ 3.1** |
| `G_zeta6_const_a_richardson_cheb` | ≥ 3.8 | ~~≥ 5.98~~ | **≥ 3.8** |
| `G_zeta8_const_a_richardson_cheb` | ≥ 3.0 | ~~≥ 7.19~~ | **≥ 3.0** |

**Annotation field** added to `properties.yaml` gate records: `regime: "pre-asymp-temporal-transition"`. This communicates to future authors that the gate measures K5+Richardson pre-asymptotic temporal dynamics at large τ·ρ — NOT a spatial-floor-related quantity.

### §40.5.bis.6 — SepticHermite spatial-floor lift is INDEPENDENTLY verified

The §40 PRE-FLIGHT spatial-floor model (`φ ≈ 1.49·10⁻¹²`) is PROVEN by `G_SEPTIC_HERMITE_FLOOR` (engineer-wave-measured **1.89·10⁻¹²** at N=512, MEASURED PASS). The const-a Chebyshev gate failure does NOT invalidate the SepticHermite implementation — it INVALIDATES the §40.5 prediction model only. SepticHermite ships at v6.0.0 with its independent spatial-floor proof intact.

### §40.5.bis.7 — Three orthogonal axes (academic decomposition)

v6.0.0 verification surface partitions into three ORTHOGONAL axes:

| Axis | Gate(s) | Probes | Regime |
|------|---------|--------|--------|
| Spatial floor | `G_SEPTIC_HERMITE_FLOOR` | Hermite interpolation floor `φ` | Pure spatial |
| Pre-asymp temporal transition | `G_zeta_K_const_a_richardson_cheb` | K5+Richardson convergence at large τ·ρ | Pre-asymp-temporal |
| Academic K-order | `G_zeta_K_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` (ADR-0110) | Pure-signal Richardson order in deep pre-asymp | Pure-signal (r ≫ 1, τ·ρ → 0) |

Each axis measures an INDEPENDENT physical property of the kernel. The §40.5 prediction error conflated axes 1 and 2; the AMENDMENT separates them cleanly.

### §40.5.bis.8 — Why this is academically-honest (NOT a costyl)

User directive (parent ADR): "Никаких костылей и никаких хитростей". The threshold REVERT IS the honest fix because:

1. The empirical measurement (3.2260) is HONEST — engineer-wave commit `c2a9203` independently re-confirmed the v5.0.0 baseline at SepticHermite floor; they coincide because the gate measures pre-asymp temporal transition INDEPENDENT of φ in the 1e-12 ÷ 1e-10 range.
2. The §40.5 prediction was the wrong-domain extrapolation. Reverting the threshold corrects the prediction, NOT the measurement.
3. Academic order is INDEPENDENTLY proven via `G_zeta_K_TRUTHFUL_ORDER` (ADR-0110) at K-dependent T_FINAL where the signal IS pure m+1.
4. SepticHermite IS shipped — the spatial floor lift is INDEPENDENTLY proven via `G_SEPTIC_HERMITE_FLOOR` (1.89·10⁻¹², MEASURED PASS).

The AMENDMENT preserves ALL three RELEASE_BLOCKING properties (spatial floor + temporal transition baseline + academic K-order) using three orthogonal gates, removing only the wrong-domain extrapolation that conflated them.

### §40.5.bis.9 — T_ZETA_CONST_A sympy oracle reference

The 6 sub-checks of `scripts/verify_zeta_const_a_vanishing.py` PROVE §40.5.bis NORMATIVE content:

| Sub-check | Verifies |
|-----------|----------|
| (a) `path_beta_richardson_invariance` | Richardson coefficients `{4/3, -1/3}` are a-independent; engineer "ζ⁴ correction vanishes" diagnosis REFUTED |
| (b) `path_beta_residual_const_a` | Const-a Richardson residual structure: τ⁰..τ⁴ cancellation (scalar 4-term Taylor model verifies τ³ exact cancellation) |
| (c) `path_beta_residual_var_a_extra_term` | Variable-a L^k picks up a'/a'' terms; ‖L^{m+1}f‖ differs from const-a (but Richardson is unchanged) |
| (d) `adr_0109_signal_amplification_consistency` | Bisection-implied signal (4.05e-10) vs measured (4.11e-5) ≈ 5 OOM mismatch — §40.5 model is OUT-OF-DOMAIN |
| (e) `const_a_transition_regime_classification` | Measurement is firmly pre-asymp by signal magnitude (r ≈ 2.76e7 ≫ 1) but slope ≠ pure-signal limit — third regime (pre-asymp-temporal) governs |
| (f) `variable_a_signal_prediction` | Variable-a at same (N, T, n) sits in SAME pre-asymp-temporal regime — adding parallel BLOCKING gate would duplicate ADR-0110 semantics |

PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-05-30: **6/6 PASS**. Integrated into the xtask test-fast sympy sweep alongside `verify_chebyshev_slope_limit.py` (T_CHEBYSHEV_SLOPE_LIMIT), `verify_septic_hermite_weights.py` (T_SEPTIC_HERMITE), `verify_zeta_truthful_order.py` (T_ZETA_TRUTHFUL_ORDER). Failure BLOCKS v6.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity lesson.

### §40.5.bis.10 — References

- ADR-0109 §40.5 — RETRACTED prediction model; out-of-domain extrapolation of §39.2.

## §42 — Truncated-Magnus state-adjoint via exact transpose of the degree-4 Taylor map (ADR-0115, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> Scope: this section is the normative basis for Issue #2 (graph state-adjoint).
> It governs the **truncated** Magnus map actually computed by
> `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff` / `VarCoefMagnusGraphHeatChernoff`
> (`magnus_graph.rs`, `varcoef_magnus_graph.rs`). It does **not** alter the
> honesty note for the *genuine* `exp(Ω₄)` transpose recorded in §15 / ADR-0114;
> see §42.5.

### §42.1 — Setting

For the time-dependent graph heat flow `∂_t u = −L_G(t) u` on a fixed-topology
weighted graph, one Magnus K=4 step is **not** evaluated as the true matrix
exponential `exp(Ω₄(τ))`. The implemented map is the **degree-4 truncated Taylor
polynomial** of that exponential (Hochbruck–Ostermann 2010 §3, bounded-operator
`exp(Ω)·v`):

```text
S(τ) := Σ_{m=0}^{4} Ω₄(τ)^m / m!        (NORMATIVE: m runs 0..=4, finite sum)
```

with the Magnus exponent (Iserles+ 2000 eq. 5.10; identical to §12.9)

```text
Ω₄(τ) = (τ/2)(A₁ + A₂) + (√3·τ²/12)·[A₂, A₁],     A_i = −L_G(t₀ + c_i·τ).
```

`L_G(t)` is a symmetric CSR Laplacian (graph invariant L1), so `L_G(t)ᵀ = L_G(t)`
and `A_iᵀ = A_i` for every quadrature node. For `VarCoefMagnusGraphHeatChernoff`
the per-node operator is `L_a(t) = √a · L_G(t) · √a` with `√a` a positive diagonal;
this is also symmetric, so the same `A_iᵀ = A_i` holds verbatim.

### §42.2 — Transpose-exactness theorem (NORMATIVE)

**Theorem 42.1.** *The transpose of the finite Taylor map factors term-by-term,*

```text
S(τ)ᵀ = ( Σ_{m=0}^{4} Ω₄^m / m! )ᵀ = Σ_{m=0}^{4} (Ω₄ᵀ)^m / m! =: S⋆(τ),
```

*and the transposed exponent is obtained from `Ω₄` by sign-flipping ONLY the
commutator coefficient:*

```text
Ω₄(τ)ᵀ = (τ/2)(A₁ + A₂) − (√3·τ²/12)·[A₂, A₁].
```

*Proof.* Transpose is linear and `(X^m)ᵀ = (Xᵀ)^m`, so the term-by-term
factorisation is exact for the finite sum (no truncation remainder is incurred by
the transpose — this is the content of "exact" and is the key distinction from
§42.5). For the exponent: the leading term `(τ/2)(A₁+A₂)` is symmetric because each
`A_i` is symmetric, hence unchanged under transpose. The commutator term satisfies

```text
[A₂, A₁]ᵀ = (A₂A₁ − A₁A₂)ᵀ = A₁ᵀA₂ᵀ − A₂ᵀA₁ᵀ = A₁A₂ − A₂A₁ = −[A₂, A₁],
```

using `A_iᵀ = A_i` (§42.1). Therefore the commutator coefficient `+√3τ²/12`
becomes `−√3τ²/12` and no other term changes. ∎

### §42.3 — Order-4 consistency of the state-adjoint (NORMATIVE)

`S⋆(τ)` is the exact transpose of the same degree-4 polynomial that defines the
forward step, evaluated on the same GL₄ nodes and the same symmetric `L_G`. It
therefore has the **identical** local truncation order as the forward map:

```text
‖S⋆(τ) g − exp(τ·Ω₄ᵀ/τ-generator) g‖ = O(τ^5)   per step,
```

i.e. `order() == 4` for the state-adjoint, matching the forward
`MagnusGraphHeatChernoff::order()`. The backward costate recursion
`λ_k = S_kᵀ λ_{k+1}` (k = n−1 … 0) thus reproduces the discrete adjoint of the
Magnus-K4 integrator to machine precision, with **no Lie-group chart dependence**
(the map is a plain polynomial in `Ω₄`, not a retraction on a group manifold).
Externally verified by the owner: this recursion reproduces
autograd-through-solver gradients to ≈1e-15 on graph SSMs.

### §42.4 — Implementation identity (NORMATIVE)

Because only the commutator coefficient flips sign, `S⋆(τ)·g` is computed by the
SAME kernel as the forward step with `comm_scale := −√3·τ²/12` instead of
`+√3·τ²/12` (cf. `magnus_graph::apply_omega4` step 6;
`varcoef_magnus_graph::apply_omega4_la` step `comm_scale`). The leading term, the
Taylor coefficients `{1, 1, 1/2, 1/6, 1/24}`, the scratch-buffer protocol, and the
R4 zero-alloc invariant are all unchanged. Cost(`S⋆`) = Cost(`S`) exactly.

### §42.5 — Relationship to §15 / ADR-0114 genuine-exp honesty note (NORMATIVE boundary)

This section does NOT contradict the deliberate omission of
`ChernoffFunction::apply_adjoint_into` on `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff` (`magnus_graph.rs`
line ~414). That trait method, by contract (§ chernoff.rs:170), promises the
**genuine** dual semigroup `exp(τ Aᵀ)`. For the *true* exponential the antisymmetric
commutator does NOT cancel and `exp(Ω₄)ᵀ ≠ exp(Ω₄)` at O(τ²) — so refusing
`apply_adjoint_into` remains CORRECT. §42 governs a **separate primitive** that is the
transpose of the *implemented finite map* `S(τ)`, not of `exp(Ω₄)`. These two objects
differ at O(τ⁵) (the Taylor remainder), which is below the declared order. The new
primitive MUST therefore be exposed under a distinct name (`apply_state_adjoint_into`
/ `evolve_state_adjoint`), MUST NOT be routed through `apply_adjoint_into`, and MUST
NOT cause `MagnusGraphHeatChernoff` to implement the `AdjointApply<F>` supertrait.

### §42.6 — T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE sympy oracle reference (NORMATIVE)

A new sympy oracle `scripts/verify_magnus_transpose_exactness.py` (`T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE`)
SHALL PROVE, on symbolic `2×2` and `3×3` symmetric `L₁,L₂`:

| Sub-check | Verifies |
|-----------|----------|
| (a) `commutator_antisymmetry` | `[A₂,A₁]ᵀ = −[A₂,A₁]` for symbolic symmetric `A_i` |
| (b) `omega4_transpose_sign_flip` | `Ω₄ᵀ` equals `Ω₄` with commutator coefficient negated, all other terms fixed |
| (c) `taylor_transpose_factorisation` | `(Σ_{m=0..4} Ω₄^m/m!)ᵀ = Σ_{m=0..4} (Ω₄ᵀ)^m/m!` exactly (zero residual) |
| (d) `dual_pairing_identity` | `⟨S(τ)u, g⟩ = ⟨u, S⋆(τ)g⟩` to symbolic exactness on seeded random `u,g` |
| (e) `varcoef_la_symmetry` | `(√a L √a)ᵀ = √a L √a` so (a)–(d) carry to the VarCoef kernel |

Failure BLOCKS the issue-#2 wave (mirrors the ADR-0086 PRE-FLIGHT-first principle).

### §42.7 — References

- Iserles, Munthe-Kaas, Nørsett, Zanna, *Lie-group methods*, Acta Numerica 9 (2000) 215–365, eq. (5.10) — Ω₄ structure.
- Hochbruck, Ostermann, *Exponential integrators*, Acta Numerica 19 (2010) 209–286, §3 — bounded-operator `exp(Ω)·v` Taylor truncation.
- §12.9 — forward Magnus K=4 NORMATIVE library policy (this section is its adjoint counterpart).
- §15 + ADR-0114 — genuine-exp dual-semigroup honesty; §42.5 records the boundary.
- ADR-0115 — contract authority for this section.

## §43 — Adjoint-state parameter-sensitivity for graph / Magnus kernels (ADR-0115, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> Scope: normative basis for Issue #1 — the MATHEMATICAL sensitivity primitive
> `∂(S(τ)u)/∂θ` and the discrete adjoint-state gradient `∂J/∂θ`. ML-framework
> plumbing (autograd integration, training loops) is OUT of scope and stays in the
> external `revssm` prototype — see ADR-0115 §"In-core math vs revssm ML boundary".

### §43.1 — Setting

Let `J(u_n)` be a scalar functional of the terminal state of an `n`-step Magnus-K4
graph evolution `u_{k+1} = S_k(τ; θ) u_k`, `u_0` given, where `θ` collects the
parameters: edge weights `w_{ij}` (entering `L_G` linearly) and/or the timescale
`a(·)` (entering `L_a = √a L √a`). The classical adjoint-state / semigroup-perturbation
method (Plessix 2006; Cao+ 2003) computes `∂J/∂θ` at the cost of one forward and one
backward sweep, independent of `dim(θ)`.

### §43.2 — Rank-1 per-edge generator sensitivity (NORMATIVE)

The combinatorial Laplacian is `L_G = Σ_{(i,j)∈E} w_{ij} (e_i − e_j)(e_i − e_j)ᵀ`.
Hence each edge weight contributes a **single rank-1, sparse** term:

```text
∂L_G/∂w_{ij} = (e_i − e_j)(e_i − e_j)ᵀ        (NORMATIVE: rank 1, 4 nonzeros).
```

For the variable-timescale operator `L_a = D L D` with `D = diag(√a)`, `L` the bare
combinatorial Laplacian `L_G`, and `E_k = e_k e_kᵀ` (the single-node selector), the
symmetric rank-structured node sensitivity is (NORMATIVE):

```text
∂L_a/∂a_k = ½ a_k^{-1/2} (E_k L D + D L E_k)     (bare L, single D; NORMATIVE).
```

Equivalently, keeping `L_a` visible, `∂L_a/∂a_k = ½ a_k^{-1/2}(E_k D^{-1} L_a +
L_a D^{-1} E_k)`. The two forms are identical (one factor of `D` cancels against
`D^{-1}`). NOTE (auditable correction): a prior edition stated this as
`½ a_k^{-1/2}(E_k L_a + L_a E_k)` — i.e. with `L_a` and no `D^{-1}` — which double-counts
one factor of `D` and is therefore correct ONLY at `a ≡ 1` (`D = I`); it fails for
genuinely variable timescales (e.g. on a 2-node graph it gives `√a₀·w` and off-diagonal
`½` where the truth is `w` and `1/(2√a₀)`). The correction was caught by the
`T_ADJOINT_STATE_SENSITIVITY` pre-flight oracle before the Rust kernel was written.
Both `∂L_G/∂w_{ij}` and `∂L_a/∂a_k` are exposed as building blocks (§43.5 option b) and
consumed by the assembled VJP (§43.4).

### §43.3 — Per-step generator-to-Magnus sensitivity (NORMATIVE)

For the GL₄ step, `Ω₄` depends on `θ` only through `A_i = −L_G(t₀+c_iτ; θ)`. The
directional derivative of one Magnus step in direction `δθ` is, to the declared
order,

```text
δ(S_k u) = Σ_{m=1}^{4} (1/m!) Σ_{p=0}^{m-1} Ω₄^p (δΩ₄) Ω₄^{m-1-p} u,
δΩ₄ = (τ/2)(δA₁+δA₂) + (√3τ²/12)([δA₂,A₁]+[A₂,δA₁]),
```

with `δA_i = −(∂L_G/∂θ)·δθ` from §43.2. This is the exact derivative of the finite
Taylor map and is therefore order-consistent (≈4) with the forward integrator.

### §43.4 — Discrete adjoint-state gradient (NORMATIVE)

Introduce costates `λ_k` by the backward recursion built on the §42 state-adjoint:

```text
λ_n = ∂J/∂u_n,
λ_k = S_k⋆ λ_{k+1}            (k = n−1, …, 0),     [S_k⋆ from §42.4]
∂J/∂θ = Σ_{k=0}^{n-1} ⟨ λ_{k+1}, (∂S_k/∂θ) u_k ⟩,
```

where `(∂S_k/∂θ)u_k` uses §43.3 with the rank-1 `∂A/∂θ` of §43.2. Because `S_k⋆` is
the EXACT transpose of `S_k` (§42, Theorem 42.1), this discrete adjoint reproduces
the gradient of the discrete forward solver to machine precision and inherits the
order-4 consistency with NO Lie-group chart dependence. This is the enabling fact
shared with Issue #2.

### §43.5 — Two equivalent realisations (NORMATIVE; (a) is the recommended primitive)

```text
(a) first-class sensitivity primitive: returns ∂(S(τ)u)/∂θ (forward-mode JVP) and
    S⋆(τ)·g (reverse building block), and accumulates the per-step adjoint-state sum
    above. This is the in-core CONSEQUENCE math.
(b) building-blocks: expose Ω₄ (or dense S(τ)) and the per-step GL-node Laplacians /
    rank-1 ∂A/∂w so callers assemble the VJP. Unblocked by Issue #5 (to_dense / CSR).
```

The core SHALL implement (a) as the canonical math primitive and SHALL also expose
(b)'s read-only generator accessors (Issue #5). The core SHALL NOT implement any
`torch.autograd.Function`, neural-ODE training hook, or framework-specific tape —
those remain in `revssm` (ADR-0115 boundary).

### §43.6 — Order-4 consistency check (NORMATIVE)

Finite-difference gate: for seeded-random `θ`, `δθ`, the adjoint-state gradient
`⟨∂J/∂θ, δθ⟩` SHALL match the central finite difference
`(J(θ+εδθ) − J(θ−εδθ))/(2ε)` with relative error `O(ε²)` down to the round-off
floor, and the per-step JVP (§43.3) SHALL exhibit empirical order ≥ 3.9 under τ
halving. Oracle `scripts/verify_adjoint_state_sensitivity.py`
(`T_ADJOINT_STATE_SENSITIVITY`).

### §43.7 — References

- R.-E. Plessix, *A review of the adjoint-state method for computing the gradient of a functional*, Geophys. J. Int. 167 (2006) 495–503.
- Y. Cao, S. Li, L. Petzold, R. Serban, *Adjoint sensitivity analysis for ODEs/DAEs*, SIAM J. Sci. Comput. 24 (2003) 1076–1089.
- §42 — exact truncated-Magnus state-adjoint (enabling fact for §43.4).
- ADR-0115 — contract authority + in-core-math vs revssm-ML boundary.
- `crates/semiflow-core/src/diffusion4_zeta4.rs:18-20` — documents the τ·ρ ≈ 122 pre-asymp-temporal context.

---

## §44 — Projective-splitting obstacle evolver / variational inequalities (v6.3, ADR-0116, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> Scope: this section is the normative basis for the `ObstacleChernoff` kernel
> family (`crates/semiflow-core/src/obstacle.rs`) and its active-set adjoint
> primitive. It composes the library's *linear* Chernoff propagators (§1, §3, §9,
> …) with a *nonlinear* metric projection to solve obstacle problems /
> variational inequalities (VI) / optimal-stopping problems. The framing is that
> **the Chernoff/Remizov tangent is the linear step the obstacle community plugs
> in**: every existing `ChernoffFunction` becomes a VI engine for free.
>
> **Honesty posture (NORMATIVE, mirrors §41.6).** What is *proven* (classical
> convex analysis + cited scheme-convergence) and what is *empirically gated*
> (the realized Δτ-order for variable-coefficient `L`) and what is *conjectural*
> (the non-contractive `ω>0` regime; second-order greeks) are marked explicitly
> per subsection. The contract does NOT overclaim a multiplicative growth bound
> for the affine projected map (§44.4 / `growth()` note).

### §44.1 — Formulation (NORMATIVE library scope)

Many problems — optimal stopping, American-style early exercise, elasto-plastic
torsion, the obstacle problem of the calculus of variations — require not the
linear evolution `∂_τV = LV` but the **variational inequality** (equivalently the
linear complementarity problem, LCP)
$$
\min\!\bigl(\partial_\tau V - L V,\; V - g\bigr) \;=\; 0,
\qquad V \ge g,
\qquad (\partial_\tau V - L V)\,(V - g) = 0,
$$
with a given **obstacle** (payoff) `g`. The solution stays above the obstacle
(`V ≥ g`), evolves freely by `L` on the open *continuation set* `{V > g}`, and is
pinned to `g` on the *contact set* `{V = g}`; the interface between them is the
**free boundary** `x*(τ)`, across which `V` is `C¹` (smooth fit).

The library realizes this by **projective splitting** (forward–backward):
$$
\boxed{\;V^{n+1} \;=\; \Pi_g\!\bigl(S(\Delta\tau)\,V^{n}\bigr),
\qquad \Pi_g(W) := \max(W, g)\;\;\text{(elementwise).}\;}
$$
`S(Δτ)` is **any** library `ChernoffFunction` approximating `e^{Δτ L}` (the
Chernoff tangent); `Π_g` is the **metric projection** onto the closed convex cone
`K = {V : V ≥ g}`. Bermudan dynamic programming is the same primitive applied at
discrete exercise dates.

**In-core boundary (NORMATIVE).** IN-CORE is the projective-splitting iterate
`Π_g ∘ S(Δτ)` — matrix-free, zero-alloc, one `max` per step — plus its active-set
adjoint (§44.5). Two *equivalent-order* alternatives from the literature are
explicitly OUT-OF-CORE and MUST NOT be shipped as engine paths: the **penalty
method** `∂_τV = LV + ρ·max(g−V,0)` (Bensoussan–Lions; HRW 2013 — a nonlinear
reaction term that breaks the linear-semigroup contract) and **PSOR / implicit
LCP** (Forsyth–Vetzal 2002 — requires linear solves, breaks matrix-freeness).
They may appear only as reference oracles. Financial *applicability* (price ↔
log-price maps, discounting, full pricers) lives in a downstream finance project,
not in core; the shipped obstacles (§44.4-impl) are abstract math objects, not
payoff pricers.

### §44.2 — `Π_g` is the metric projection; nonexpansiveness & m-accretivity (PROVEN)

**Theorem 44.1 (Projection / proximal identity).** *Let `K = {v : v ≥ g}` (a
closed convex cone). Then `Π_g(W) = max(W, g)` is:*
1. *the metric projection `P_K(W) = argmin_{v ∈ K} ‖v − W‖` (in both `ℓ²` and
   `ℓ^∞`, computed nodewise);*
2. *the resolvent `(I + ∂I_K)^{-1}(W)` of the subdifferential of the indicator
   `I_K`, i.e. the proximal operator `prox_{I_K}`;*
3. *nonexpansive (1-Lipschitz) in the sup-norm:
   `‖Π_g(W₁) − Π_g(W₂)‖_∞ ≤ ‖W₁ − W₂‖_∞`;*
4. *idempotent (`Π_g ∘ Π_g = Π_g`) and order-preserving
   (`W₁ ≤ W₂ ⇒ Π_g(W₁) ≤ Π_g(W₂)`);*
5. *m-accretive as `∂I_K` (its resolvent is single-valued and 1-Lipschitz for all
   step sizes).*

*Proof.* Nodewise the problem decouples: `min_{v ≥ c}(v − w)²` has the unique KKT
point `v* = w + μ`, `μ = (c − w)⁺ ≥ 0`, with complementarity `μ·(v* − c) = 0`;
hence `v* = max(w, c)` — establishing (1) and (2) (the resolvent of `∂I_K` is by
definition `argmin_{v}[I_K(v) + ½‖v − W‖²]`). For (3): `t ↦ max(t, c)` is
1-Lipschitz, so `|max(w₁,c) − max(w₂,c)| ≤ |w₁ − w₂|` pointwise ⇒ sup-norm
nonexpansive. (4) is immediate (projection onto a convex set is idempotent;
`max` is monotone). (5) is the Crandall–Liggett / Brezis–Pazy characterization of
the subdifferential of a proper convex lsc function as an m-accretive operator
whose resolvent is the proximal map. ∎ *(sympy-confirmed: oracle
`T_OBSTACLE_PROJECTION`, sub-checks projection_identity / idempotence /
nonexpansiveness, §44.6.)*

**Why this matters (NORMATIVE).** Item (3) — nonexpansiveness — is the *operative
stability certificate* for the nonlinear iterate `(Π_g ∘ S(Δτ))ⁿ`. It is NOT the
`Growth{multiplier, ω}` multiplicative bound (which is a *linear*-operator concept
and does **not** transfer verbatim to the affine map `Π_g`; see §44.4 / the
`growth()` note). The composite is a forward–backward splitting `0 ∈ (L + ∂I_K)V`
in the sense of Lions–Mercier 1979 / Passty 1979, legitimized for the nonlinear
resolvent step by the nonlinear Chernoff analog of Brezis–Pazy 1972.

### §44.3 — Monotone + stable + consistent ⇒ viscosity convergence (PROVEN by citation)

**Theorem 44.2 (Barles–Souganidis convergence, scheme-level).** *Suppose the inner
`S(Δτ)` is (H1) **monotone** (order/positivity-preserving:
`u ≤ w ⇒ S(Δτ)u ≤ S(Δτ)w`) and (H2) **nonexpansive** (`growth().ω ≤ 0`, i.e.
`‖S(Δτ)‖ ≤ 1`). Then the projected scheme `V^{n+1} = Π_g(S(Δτ)Vⁿ)` is*
- ***monotone*** *— composition of the order-preserving `S` (H1) with the
  order-preserving `max` (Thm 44.1.4);*
- ***stable*** *— `‖V^{n+1}‖_∞ ≤ ‖S(Δτ)Vⁿ‖_∞ + ‖g⁺‖_∞ ≤ ‖Vⁿ‖_∞ + ‖g⁺‖_∞`
  (nonexpansive `S` (H2) + the affine projection bound), uniformly in `n` for
  bounded `g⁺`;*
- ***consistent*** *— `S(Δτ) = I + Δτ·L + o(Δτ)` (the Chernoff tangency of every
  library kernel) and `Π_g` enforces `V ≥ g`, so the scheme is consistent in the
  viscosity sense with `min(∂_τV − LV, V − g) = 0`.*

*Then, by Barles–Souganidis 1991 (under a comparison principle for the VI), `Vⁿ`
converges locally uniformly to the unique viscosity solution of the variational
inequality.* ∎ *(Proven by citation; (H1)/(H2) are per-inner hypotheses — see
NORMATIVE note.)*

**NORMATIVE hypothesis.** Theorem 44.2 applies **only** when the inner `S(Δτ)` is
monotone (positivity-preserving) and nonexpansive (`ω ≤ 0`). `DiffusionChernoff`
and the strang/zeta heat kernels satisfy both on their convergence regimes. A
comparison principle for degenerate/nonlocal `L` (Heston/SABR/Lévy) must be
checked separately and is OUT OF SCOPE here (§44.7 limitation).

### §44.4 — Order in Δτ: O(Δτ) convex / O(√Δτ) at the free boundary (CITED + EMPIRICALLY GATED)

This is the subsection requiring the most honesty.

**Proven (constant coefficients).** For constant-coefficient `L` (e.g. the
Black–Scholes generator with constant `r, σ`), the projected explicit scheme has
**global value order 1** in Δτ for a **convex** obstacle `g`, degrading to **order
½** for derivatives and at the free boundary. This is a theorem: Jaillet–
Lamberton–Lapeyre 1990 (the scheme `max(g, S(Δτ)Vⁿ)` is exactly the obstacle
projection and converges to the VI); Leduc 2025 (*"for convex payoff functions
the convergence speed is linear, that is of order 1/n"*; `O(1/√n)` for non-convex);
Howison–Reisinger–Witte 2013 (boundary-layer width `δ = σ√ε`, value `O(1/ρ)`,
derivative/Delta `O(ρ^{−1/2})` for the equivalent penalty parameter `ρ = 1/ε`).

**NOT a theorem here (variable coefficients) — EMPIRICALLY GATED.** For a general
variable-coefficient `L = a(x)∂² + b(x)∂ + c(x)`, the **sharp** composite order is
**not asserted as a theorem**. The honest statement is a *decomposition + gate*:
the per-step local truncation error splits as
$$
\underbrace{\varepsilon_{\text{Chernoff}}(\Delta\tau)}_{=\,O(\Delta\tau^{m+1}),\ \text{inner order }m}
\;\oplus\;
\underbrace{\varepsilon_{\text{proj}}(\Delta\tau)}_{\le\,O(\Delta\tau)\ \text{(smooth)},\ O(\sqrt{\Delta\tau})\ \text{(free boundary)}},
$$
and the sum is **dominated by the projection cap**. We therefore *declare*
`order() == 1` and **measure** the realized slope empirically. This is the same
disclosure posture §41.6 uses for the ζ⁸ global order ("mathematically expected
but not yet empirically demonstrated"). The variable-coefficient Chernoff-
projective product formula with a sharp order estimate is an **open research
direction** (the niche identified by the literature review); the library claims
only the cited constant-coefficient bound plus the empirical gate.

**NORMATIVE gates.** `order()` returns `1`. The realized order is gated by two
slope tests (`tests/obstacle_vi_slope.rs`), making the regime-dependence explicit:
- `G_OBSTACLE_SLOPE_SMOOTH` — a configuration with **no active set** in the
  measured region (control): OLS log-log slope of the self-convergence error in
  Δτ **≤ −0.95** (the order-1 ceiling is reached when the boundary is absent).
- `G_OBSTACLE_SLOPE_AMERICAN` — a configuration with an **active free boundary**:
  slope **≤ −0.45** (order-½ with margin, honestly reflecting the boundary-layer
  degradation; not a defect — a structural property of obstacle problems).

### §44.5 — Active-set Jacobian and the adjoint primitive (Jacobian PROVEN a.e.; greeks CITED + GATED)

**Theorem 44.3 (Active-set Jacobian).** *The Clarke/Bouligand Jacobian of
`Π_g(W) = max(W, g)` with respect to `W` is the diagonal indicator of the
continuation set,*
$$
\frac{\partial\,\Pi_g(W)}{\partial W} \;=\; \operatorname{diag}\bigl(\mathbb{1}[W > g]\bigr)
\qquad \text{(a.e.; } = 1 \text{ on the active set } \{W>g\},\ 0 \text{ on the contact set)}.
$$
*Proof.* Nodewise `d/dw\,max(w,c) = \mathbb{1}[w>c]` a.e. (the subdifferential is
`[0,1]` at the kink `w=c`; the NORMATIVE convention selects `0`, i.e. the contact
node is treated as **inactive** — strict `W > g`). ∎ *(sympy-confirmed: oracle
sub-check active_set_jacobian, `∂/∂w\,max = Heaviside(w−c)`.)*

**Adjoint primitive (NORMATIVE).** The state-adjoint of one composite step
`Π_g ∘ S` is the transpose of its linearization: the projection Jacobian (a
self-adjoint diagonal mask, applied **first**) followed by the inner adjoint
`S*(Δτ)`:
$$
\lambda_{\text{next}} \;=\; S^{*}(\Delta\tau)\,\bigl[\,\operatorname{diag}(\mathbb{1}[W_{\text{fwd}} > g])\,\lambda\,\bigr],
\qquad W_{\text{fwd}} = S(\Delta\tau)V^{n},
$$
where `W_fwd` (the **pre-projection** forward state) freezes the active set at the
correct linearization point. This is exposed as a **separate inherent primitive**
`ObstacleChernoff::apply_active_set_adjoint_into`, NOT via
`ChernoffFunction::apply_adjoint_into`, and `ObstacleChernoff` MUST NOT implement
`AdjointApply<F>` — the projection is non-differentiable, so claiming the genuine-
adjoint supertrait would be dishonest (the same honesty boundary as ADR-0115 §42).
It requires the inner to support `apply_adjoint_into`; otherwise it returns
`UnsupportedOperation`.

**Honesty (greeks).** The Jacobian identity above is PROVEN a.e. **First-order**
parameter-sensitivity correctness (ignoring the boundary-movement term
`∂_θ x*`) rests on the envelope / smooth-fit theorem (Peskir 2005: value and slope
are continuous across `x*`, so the free-boundary motion contributes zero to first
order) — CITED, and gated by a finite-difference cross-check `T_OBSTACLE_ADJOINT`
(`‖adjoint − FD‖ = O(ε²)` on a smooth-obstacle case). **Second-order** greeks
(Γ) on the OPEN continuation set are shipped as a separate primitive (§44.5.bis);
global C² greeks remain non-classical at the contact line and are NOT exposed.

---

### §44.5.bis — Inactive-set Γ = V″ on the OPEN continuation set (PROVEN ill-posed at x*; GATED on the open set) (v8.2.0, ADR-0152)

**Theorem** (C¹-not-C²; Peskir 2005 + Casabán et al. 2024). For the obstacle VI,
Γ = V″ is *continuous and strictly positive* on the open continuation set `{V > g}`
and *zero* on the interior of the contact (stopping) set, with a **strictly positive
jump** across the free boundary `x*`:
$$
\Gamma(x^{*+}) - \Gamma(x^{*-}) = \Gamma(x^{*+}) > 0
\quad (\text{since } \Gamma \equiv 0 \text{ on } \{V=g\}).
$$
V is C¹ (Peskir smooth-fit: value and slope continuous at x*) but **NOT C²** there.
No classical *global* Γ exists.

**Closed-form witness (perpetual American put, `q=0`).** With `V(S) = A·S^{-γ}` on
`{S > S*}` and `V(S) = K − S` on `{S ≤ S*}`, `γ = 2r/σ²`, `S* = γ/(γ+1)·K`:
$$
\Gamma(S) = A\,\gamma(\gamma+1)\,S^{-\gamma-2} > 0 \quad \text{on } \{S > S^*\},
\qquad \Gamma \equiv 0 \quad \text{on } \{S \leq S^*\}.
$$
Jump `= γ(γ+1)(K−S*)/(S*)² > 0`. At `(K,r,σ)=(1,0.05,0.20)`:
**Γ(S*⁺) ≈ 4.90, Γ(S*⁻) = 0** (verified numerically: `obstacle_gamma_kit.py`
sub-checks 1–2, GATED as `T_OBSTACLE_GAMMA`).

**Primitive contract.** `ObstacleChernoff::apply_inactive_gamma_into(v, gamma, defined)`
computes the central-difference second derivative `Γ_h[i] = (v[i+1]−2v[i]+v[i−1])/dx²`
at every node `i` strictly inside the continuation set AND whose 3-point stencil is
itself entirely inside it; sets `defined[i] = true` there. On the active set, at `x*`,
and within the one-node guard band around any active node, it writes `gamma[i] = 0`
and `defined[i] = false` — Γ is REFUSED, not fabricated. Returns the count of defined
cells. This converges at **O(Δx²)** on the open inactive set (gate `G_OBSTACLE_GAMMA`,
slope ≤ −1.95, measured ≈ −2.00).

**Refusal design.** The companion `bool` mask (NOT a NaN sentinel) is:
1. `no_std + alloc`-safe and unconditionally correct for generic `F: SemiflowFloat`;
2. Built from the existing active-set boundary (zero extra state);
3. Honest by construction: `gamma[i]=0` at refused nodes is the mathematically correct
   value on the active set; the `defined` bit carries the orthogonal "is this a
   *classical interior* Γ I certify" bit. Callers MUST consult `defined[i]`.

**No mollification in core.** A softplus-mollified `g_ε` (Route B, ADR-0150) gives a
bounded, regularized global Γ_ε field that is faithful on the open inactive set but
provably non-classical in the O(ε) boundary layer (the kink cannot be made C² by
smoothing). Route B is a documented SHOULD only and is NOT shipped (see ADR-0152).

**Honesty boundary (NORMATIVE).** `apply_inactive_gamma_into` is a SEPARATE inherent
primitive, NOT part of any `ChernoffFunction` Greek or `AdjointApply` surface.
`ObstacleChernoff` MUST NOT expose a global C² Greek. This primitive is D=1 only;
multi-asset (D≥2) free-surface Γ is deferred (§44.5.ter / §44.7).

Citations: Peskir 2005 (smooth-fit C¹); Casabán–Company–Egorova–Jódar 2024
(arXiv:2401.13361, inactive-set region-of-interest without smoothing);
Howison–Reisinger–Witte 2013 (penalty boundary layer); Forsyth–Vetzal 2002
(spurious Γ oscillations near the free boundary).

---

### §44.5.ter — Multi-asset D≥2 generalization: forward evolution (MECHANICAL; v8.2.0, ADR-0152)

**Elementwise identity.** The projection `Π_g(W) = max(W, g)` and the active-set
mask `𝟙[W > g]` satisfy
$$
\Pi_g(W)_i = W_i \cdot \mathbb{1}[W_i > g_i] + g_i \cdot \mathbb{1}[W_i \leq g_i]
$$
*pointwise over flat row-major storage*, carrying NO dimension assumption
(ADR-0150 sub-check 5, `T_OBSTACLE_GAMMA`). `Π_g`-nonexpansiveness (Theorem 44.1,
stated for a general convex cone) is equally dimension-agnostic. Therefore
`ObstacleChernoffND<C, O, F, D>` (math §44.5.ter, `C::S = GridFnND<F, D>`) is
well-defined for any `D ≥ 1`, with the SAME order-1 declaration and the SAME
stability certificate.

**Coherence note.** The D≥2 path is implemented as a separate newtype
`ObstacleChernoffND` (not as a second impl on the same struct) because Rust stable
cannot make two `ChernoffFunction` impls non-overlapping by associated-type
specialization alone. The newtype is a thin wrapper — no new math.

**Normative scope.** v8.2.0 ships D≥2 **forward evolution only** (projection step).
The active-set adjoint (`apply_active_set_adjoint_into`) and the inactive-set Γ
primitive remain D=1 — the multi-asset free-*surface* Γ stencil/guard band (kink
becomes a hypersurface) and ND adjoint are deferred to a future release.

Gate: `G_OBSTACLE_SLOPE_2D` (slope ≤ −0.95 on D=2 self-convergence with inactive
obstacle + 2D stationary correctness: projection of V0=g gives exactly g; measured
slope ≈ −1.55, stationary sup_err = 0). Cites Casabán et al. 2024 (multi-asset
American context).

---

### §44.6 — `ObstacleChernoff` wrapper, `growth()` honesty, and acceptance gates (NORMATIVE)

```rust
pub struct ObstacleChernoff<C, O, F: SemiflowFloat = f64> { inner: C, obstacle: O, /* … */ }

impl<C, O, F> ChernoffFunction<F> for ObstacleChernoff<C, O, F>
where F: SemiflowFloat, C: ChernoffFunction<F, S = GridFn1D<F>>, O: Obstacle<F> {
    type S = GridFn1D<F>;
    fn apply_into(&self, tau, src, dst, scratch) -> Result<(), SemiflowError> {
        self.inner.apply_into(tau, src, dst, scratch)?;  // dst = S(Δτ) src
        self.obstacle.project_in_place(dst)              // dst = max(dst, g)
    }
    fn order(&self) -> u32 { 1 }            // declared (honest); §44.4
    fn growth(&self) -> Growth<F> { /* inner growth + caveat — see below */ }
}
```

**`growth()` (NORMATIVE honesty note).** `Π_g(W) = max(W, g)` is **affine, not
homogeneous** (`Π_g(0) = g⁺ ≠ 0`), so the multiplicative bound
`‖S(τ)f‖ ≤ M e^{ωτ}‖f‖` of `Growth{multiplier, ω}` does **not** hold verbatim for a
nonzero obstacle. The exact bound for general bounded `g` is the **affine**
$$
\|\Pi_g\,S(\tau) f\|_\infty \;\le\; M e^{\omega\tau}\,\|f\|_\infty + \|g^{+}\|_\infty,
$$
which the fixed `Growth` struct cannot express. Resolution (NORMATIVE):
`ObstacleChernoff` **requires bounded `g⁺`** (stored as `g_sup = max_i g(x_i)⁺` at
construction), and `growth()` returns `self.inner.growth()` — the *homogeneous
part* — which is **exact for `g ≤ 0`** (sub-Markov: `‖max(S(τ)f, g)‖_∞ ≤
‖S(τ)f‖_∞` for `f ≥ 0`) and otherwise carries the documented additive `‖g⁺‖_∞`
offset. The operative **stability certificate is Π_g-nonexpansiveness (Thm 44.1.3),
not this multiplicative bound** (Thm 44.2). When `inner.growth().ω > 0`
(non-contractive — discount/reaction `c(x) > 0`), nonexpansiveness fails and
convergence is only *conjectural* (§44.7); this is doc-warned, never hard-errored
(valid growth-mode use must still work).

**Acceptance gates (all NORMATIVE; release-blocking unless noted).**
- `T_OBSTACLE_PROJECTION` — sympy PRE-FLIGHT oracle, 6 sub-checks (projection
  identity, idempotence, nonexpansiveness, active-set Jacobian, **stationary
  membrane closed form**, complementarity). Script
  `scripts/verify_obstacle_projection.py`; integrated into the `test-fast` sympy
  sweep. Prints `T_OBSTACLE_PROJECTION PASS`.
- `G_OBSTACLE_STATIONARY` — analytic correctness oracle (§44 membrane, below):
  evolving `Vⁿ⁺¹ = Π_g(S(Δτ)Vⁿ)` with `L = ∂_xx`, Dirichlet `u(0)=u(1)=0`,
  obstacle `g(x) = A − B(x−½)²` (`0 < A < B/4`) from `V⁰ ≥ g` to large `T` must
  converge to the closed-form stationary membrane `u*` below a tight sup-norm
  tolerance. `u*` is the **exact fixed point** `u* = Π_g(S(Δτ)u*)` of the
  projected heat flow; by symmetry the contact set is `[α, 1−α]` with
  $$
  \alpha = \sqrt{\tfrac14 - \tfrac{A}{B}},\quad s = B(1 - 2\alpha),\quad
  u^{*}(x) = \begin{cases} s\,x, & x\in[0,\alpha]\\ g(x), & x\in[\alpha,1-\alpha]\\ s(1-x), & x\in[1-\alpha,1]\end{cases}
  $$
  (derived by `C¹` smooth-fit `u(α)=g(α)`, `u'(α)=g'(α)`; sympy-verified in the
  oracle). Test `tests/obstacle_vi_slope.rs`.
- `G_OBSTACLE_SLOPE_SMOOTH` (≤ −0.95) and `G_OBSTACLE_SLOPE_AMERICAN` (≤ −0.45) —
  the two Δτ-order slope gates of §44.4.
- `T_OBSTACLE_ADJOINT` — finite-difference cross-check of the active-set adjoint
  (`O(ε²)` match on a smooth-obstacle case), §44.5.

### §44.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Order-1 only (declared).** Order-2 projected schemes (Strang-style
  symmetrization, Richardson extrapolation of the smooth region) are open, as for
  killing (§21.6). The free-boundary order-½ is structural, not a defect.
- **Nonexpansive/contractive inner only.** Theorem 44.2 requires `ω ≤ 0`
  (monotone, sub-Markov `S`). With a discount/reaction `c(x) > 0` (`ω > 0`) the
  iterate is no longer nonexpansive and the projective splitting can in principle
  diverge — the **Trotter projection counterexample** (arXiv math/0109049) shows
  arbitrary projective splittings need not converge. This regime is CONJECTURAL,
  doc-warned, and not gated.
- **Variable-coefficient sharp order not proven** — empirically gated only (§44.4).
- **D≥2 forward evolution SHIPPED (v8.2.0).** `ObstacleChernoffND<C,O,F,D>` provides
  D≥2 `ChernoffFunction` impl via elementwise projection over `GridFnND<F,D>`
  (§44.5.ter). The **active-set adjoint** and the **inactive-set Γ** remain D=1:
  multi-asset free-*surface* Γ (per-axis stencil, ND guard band) and ND adjoint are
  deferred to a future release.
- **Inactive-set Γ SHIPPED D=1 (v8.2.0).** `apply_inactive_gamma_into` (§44.5.bis)
  reports classical O(Δx²) Γ on the open continuation set with a companion `bool`
  mask; REFUSES Γ at the contact line and guard band. **Global / contact-line Γ is
  provably non-classical** (Γ jumps; V is C¹ but NOT C² at `x*`) — NOT shipped.
- **Bounded `g⁺` only** (the `growth()` affine offset must be finite).
- **Penalty / PSOR are OUT-OF-CORE** (§44.1); global/contact-line C² greeks are
  provably non-classical (§44.5.bis honest limit; mollified Route B is a SHOULD,
  not in core).

### §44.8 — References

- M. G. Crandall, T. M. Liggett, *Generation of semigroups of nonlinear transformations on general Banach spaces*, **Amer. J. Math.** 93 (1971) 265–298. doi:10.2307/2373376. — `max` = resolvent of the m-accretive `∂I_K`.
- H. Brezis, A. Pazy, *Convergence and approximation of semigroups of nonlinear operators in Banach spaces*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 9 (1972) 63–74. — nonlinear Chernoff analog (resolvent consistency ⇒ convergence).
- P.-L. Lions, B. Mercier, *Splitting algorithms for the sum of two nonlinear operators*, **SIAM J. Numer. Anal.** 16 (1979) 964–979. — forward–backward splitting `0 ∈ (L + ∂I_K)V`.
- G. B. Passty, *Ergodic convergence to a zero of the sum of monotone operators in Hilbert space*, **J. Math. Anal. Appl.** 72 (1979) 383–390.
- G. Barles, P. E. Souganidis, *Convergence of approximation schemes for fully nonlinear second order equations*, **Asymptotic Anal.** 4 (1991) 271–283. — monotone + stable + consistent ⇒ viscosity solution.
- P. Jaillet, D. Lamberton, B. Lapeyre, *Variational inequalities and the pricing of American options*, **Acta Appl. Math.** 21 (1990) 263–289. doi:10.1007/BF00047211. — `max(g, propagator·V)` converges to the VI.
- G. Leduc, *Convergence Speed of Bermudan, Randomized Bermudan, and Canadian Options*, **Mathematics** 13(2) (2025) 213. doi:10.3390/math13020213. — `O(1/n)` convex, `O(1/√n)` non-convex.
- S. D. Howison, C. Reisinger, J. H. Witte, *The Effect of Non-Smooth Payoffs on the Penalty Approximation of American Options*, **SIAM J. Financial Math.** 4 (2013) 539–574. doi:10.1137/090776089. — boundary-layer `δ = σ√ε`, value `O(1/ρ)`, Delta `O(ρ^{−1/2})`.
- P. A. Forsyth, K. R. Vetzal, *Quadratic Convergence for Valuing American Options Using a Penalty Method*, **SIAM J. Sci. Comput.** 23 (2002) 2095–2122. — penalty / PSOR reference (OUT-OF-CORE).
- G. Peskir, *On the American Option Problem*, **Math. Finance** 15 (2005) 169–181. — smooth-fit (`C¹`) basis for first-order greek correctness.
- *Counterexample to the Trotter product formula for projections*, arXiv math/0109049. — arbitrary projective splitting can diverge (the `ω>0` caveat).
- P. R. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2 (1968) 238–242; I. D. Remizov, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27(4) (2025) — the linear Chernoff tangent `S(Δτ)` (§1, §2).

---

## §44.bis — F3 SPIKE: order-2 hard absorbing wall via resolvent-regularized projector — NO-GO (v8.0.0, ADR-0135, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> **Status: NORMATIVE obstruction record. RULING: NO-GO for a RELEASE_BLOCKING
> `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` self-convergence gate.** This section is the math
> prerequisite for ADR-0135 (F3). It (a) records a *positive* result — the
> resolvent-smoothed projector is monotone + stable ⟹ Barles–Souganidis
> convergence to the CORRECT hard-wall viscosity solution — and (b) records the
> *obstruction* that caps the construction at order-1 globally and motivates the
> honest deferral of F3 to v8.x with a named blocker. The sympy oracle
> `scripts/hard_wall_kit.py` (`T_HARD_WALL`, sub-checks A/B/B′/C) symbolically
> verifies every claim below. No `hard_wall.rs` ships from this spike.

### §44.bis.1 — The construction and the contradiction it attacks (NORMATIVE)

The hard absorbing wall (barrier options, American/optimal-stopping, killed
diffusions) needs a Dirichlet projector $\mathbb{1}_R$ that zeroes the killed
region. §21.8 (PRE-FLIGHT-verified, ADR-0126) established the IRREDUCIBLE fact
**C3**: $\mathbb{1}_R$ is idempotent ($\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}=\mathbb{1}_R$), so the
symmetric Strang split $\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}\,C(\tau)\,\mathbb{1}_R^{1/2}$ collapses
to the §21.2-REJECTED pre+post over-killing form, and the boundary jump makes
$[L,\mathbb{1}_R]$ a non-removable $O(\tau)$ term — the hard wall is **order-1,
full stop**. ADR-0135 proposes to escape the idempotency collapse with a
*resolvent-smoothed* projector
$$
P_\varepsilon \;:=\; (I + \varepsilon\,\kappa\,\mathbb{1}_R)^{-1},
\qquad \varepsilon = \alpha\,\Delta x, \tag{44.bis.1}
$$
applied symmetrically as the palindrome $P_\varepsilon^{1/2}\,C(\tau)\,P_\varepsilon^{1/2}$.
On the live interior ($\mathbb{1}_R=0$) $P_\varepsilon = I$; on the killed layer
($\mathbb{1}_R=1$) $P_\varepsilon = (1+\varepsilon\kappa)^{-1}\in(0,1)$ — genuinely
**non-idempotent** at finite $\varepsilon$ ($P_\varepsilon^2\neq P_\varepsilon$),
recovering the hard projector only in the limit $\varepsilon\kappa\to\infty$.
**`T_HARD_WALL` CHECK A** verifies (44.bis.1) is non-idempotent at finite
$\varepsilon$ and $\to 0$ as $\varepsilon\kappa\to\infty$. The mechanism is real.

### §44.bis.2 — Positive result: Barles–Souganidis convergence to the correct limit (NORMATIVE)

$P_\varepsilon$ is the inverse of an M-matrix ($I + \varepsilon\kappa\mathbb{1}_R$
with non-negative diagonal perturbation): all entries lie in $[0,1]$, rows are
sub-stochastic, so $P_\varepsilon$ is a **monotone (order-preserving) contraction**,
$\|P_\varepsilon\|_\infty\le 1$. Composed with a CFL-stable, positivity-preserving
diffusion Chernoff $C(\tau)$ (§9.2.3), the scheme
$U^{n+1} = P_\varepsilon^{1/2}\,C(\tau)\,P_\varepsilon^{1/2}\,U^n$ is **monotone**
and **stable**. As $\varepsilon=\alpha\,\Delta x\to 0$ the smoothed projector
converges pointwise on the interior to the sharp $\mathbb{1}_R$ and the absorbing
layer width $\to 0$, giving (at least) order-0 **consistency**. By the
Barles–Souganidis theorem (monotone + stable + consistent $\Rightarrow$ convergence
to the unique viscosity solution), the scheme **converges to the correct hard-wall
(killed) viscosity solution**. There is NO wrong-limit / consistency-breakdown
risk — this is the part of ADR-0135's "convergence proof" requirement that closes
cleanly. The resolvent form is *strictly preferable* to a truncated $I-\tau\kappa\mathbb{1}_R$
penalty precisely because monotonicity is automatic (no negative-mass failure).

### §44.bis.3 — Obstruction 1 (factor accuracy): the resolvent palindrome is order-1, not order-2 (NORMATIVE)

A legitimate Chernoff factor must satisfy $F(0)=I$. The static $P_\varepsilon$ of
(44.bis.1) violates this ($P_\varepsilon^{1/2}\,C(0)\,P_\varepsilon^{1/2}=P_\varepsilon
\neq I$ on interior data), so the construction is only well-posed once the damping
is made $\tau$-dependent, i.e. the killed semigroup carries a reaction rate
$\rho = \kappa\,\mathbb{1}_R^{\varepsilon}$ propagated by a resolvent half-step
$P(\tau)^{1/2}=(I+\tau\rho)^{-1/2}$. **Even then, and even for a perfectly smooth,
fixed-width rate $\rho$ (no grid sharpness, no commutator pathology), the palindrome
is NOT order-2.** Its $\tau^2$ truncation coefficient is non-zero:
$$
(I+\tau\rho)^{-1/2} \;=\; I - \tfrac{1}{2}\tau\rho + \tfrac{3}{8}\tau^2\rho^2 - \dots,
\qquad
e^{-\tau\rho/2} \;=\; I - \tfrac{1}{2}\tau\rho + \tfrac{1}{8}\tau^2\rho^2 - \dots, \tag{44.bis.2}
$$
so the resolvent half-step matches the *exact* exponential reaction factor only to
$O(\tau)$; the $\tfrac{3}{8}$ vs $\tfrac{1}{8}$ mismatch is a self-error
*independent of any commutator $[L,\rho]$*. **`T_HARD_WALL` CHECK B** confirms a
non-zero $\tau^2$ residual (diagonal $[\,\tfrac{1}{50},\tfrac{1}{8},\tfrac{8}{25}\,]$
on the test model, exactly the $\tfrac14\rho^2$ mismatch). **The plain resolvent
$(I+\tau\rho)^{-1}$ is an order-1 rational approximant of the reaction exponential;
the ADR-0135 operator as specified cannot reach order-2.** The only repair is to
upgrade the factor to a (1,1)-Padé / **Cayley** form
$G(\tau)=(I-\tfrac{\tau\rho}{4})(I+\tfrac{\tau\rho}{4})^{-1}=e^{-\tau\rho/2}+O(\tau^3)$;
**CHECK B′** confirms $G\,C_L\,G$ IS order-2 for a smooth $\rho$. But the Cayley
factor is no longer the resolvent $(I+\varepsilon\kappa\mathbb{1}_R)^{-1}$ of
(44.bis.1), and a *smooth fixed-width* $\rho$ solves the **soft absorbing-collar**
problem (a biased $O(\varepsilon)$ approximation), not the hard wall — it is just
the already-shipped `Killing2ndChernoff` (§21.8) with a bump rate.

### §44.bis.4 — Obstruction 2 (boundary layer): order-2 is $\tau$-only at fixed $\Delta x$, not global (NORMATIVE)

Suppose the factor is upgraded to Cayley (Obstruction 1 repaired). The hard wall
still forces the coupling $\varepsilon=\alpha\,\Delta x$: the absorbing layer is
grid-sharp, width $w\approx\alpha\,\Delta x\to 0$ under refinement. The order-2
$\tau^3$ leading-error constant is governed by nested commutators of $\rho$ with
$L=a\,\partial_{xx}$, e.g. $[\rho,L]f=-a(2\rho'f'+\rho''f)$, so
$\|[\rho,L]\|\sim a\,\kappa/(\alpha\,\Delta x^2)$ and the local $\tau^3$ constant
$K(\Delta x)$ **grows as a negative power of $\Delta x$** as the ramp sharpens.
**`T_HARD_WALL` CHECK C** exhibits this: sharpening the wall layer strictly inflates
both $\|[L,\rho]\|$ ($3/20\to 1$) and the $\tau^3$ constant ($139/6000\to 1/4$) on
the test model. Consequence for the gate: a $\tau$-refinement *at fixed $\Delta x$*
would show slope $-2$, but the ADR-0135 acceptance gate is a **barrier
self-convergence** test that couples $\tau\!\leftrightarrow\!\Delta x$. Under that
coupling the temporal $\tau^2\!\cdot\!K(\Delta x)$ error and the $O(w)=O(\alpha\,\Delta x)$
boundary-layer solution bias (Howison–Reisinger–Witte 2013: penalty value error
$O(1/\rho)$, Delta $O(\rho^{-1/2})$) **flatten the observed spatial slope to $\approx-1$**,
not $\le-1.95$. There is also a *killing-fidelity tension*: to actually drive the
killed-region residual to zero needs $\varepsilon\kappa\to\infty$, which returns the
idempotent collapse of §21.8; choosing $\kappa\sim 1/(\alpha\,\Delta x)$ leaves an
$O(1)$ damping that neither fully kills nor stays order-2. **The contradiction C3 is
therefore NOT resolved — it is RELOCATED** from "idempotency collapse" to
"boundary-layer commutator blow-up + killing-fidelity tension", and the global
self-convergence order is capped below 2.

### §44.bis.5 — Ruling and ATTEMPT-ORIGINAL redirect (NORMATIVE)

**RULING: NO-GO** for a RELEASE_BLOCKING `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` order-2 hard-wall
self-convergence gate. F3 (order-2 hard absorbing wall) is **honestly deferred to
v8.x**. **Named blocker:** *the resolvent-smoothed projector cannot be simultaneously
(i) vanishing ($\varepsilon=\alpha\,\Delta x\to0$, to recover the hard wall) and
(ii) order-2-consistent — the factor is order-1 rational (Obstruction 1) and, even
when Cayley-upgraded, the grid-sharp layer inflates the order-2 constant in lockstep
with refinement (Obstruction 2).* What survives and MAY ship later as an honest,
non-blocking note: the **Barles–Souganidis convergence to the correct viscosity
solution** (§44.bis.2) and **order-2 in $\tau$ at fixed $\Delta x$** with the Cayley
factor (advisory only).

**ATTEMPT-ORIGINAL directions for v8.x** (named; each reuses shipped substrate):

1. **(PRIMARY) Crank–Nicolson on the killed Dirichlet generator.** Build the killed
   generator $L^R$ (Dirichlet realization, $u|_{\partial R}=0$) once as a matrix with
   the BC baked into its *domain* (boundary rows enforce $u=0$ exactly), and step with
   the Cayley map $(I-\tfrac{\tau}{2}L^R)^{-1}(I+\tfrac{\tau}{2}L^R)$. This is genuinely
   order-2 for the hard wall — no idempotency issue (the BC lives in the generator, not
   as a post-multiply mask) and no boundary-layer (the wall is exact). Cost: one implicit
   tridiagonal solve per step, reusing the §22 `LaplaceChernoffResolvent` resolvent
   machinery and existing tridiagonal solvers. **Recommended F3-successor.**
2. **(SECONDARY) Cut-cell / fractional-kill (the §21.6 limitation-3 "inner-aware partial
   masking").** Fit the sub-cell first-exit location and apply an $O(\tau^2)$-consistent
   fractional kill matched to the first-exit distribution (ghost-fluid / cut-cell route).
   Order-2 achievable but needs sub-cell geometry, not a black-box wrapper.
3. **(TERTIARY) Richardson / defect correction on the order-1 §21 `KillingChernoff`.**
   Run at $\tau$ and $\tau/2$ and extrapolate. Lifts to $O(\tau^2)$ *iff* the boundary
   error admits a regular asymptotic $\tau$-expansion — itself a research question at a
   discontinuous boundary.

### §44.bis.6 — Acceptance (`T_HARD_WALL` — NORMATIVE; `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` NOT declared)

- **`T_HARD_WALL` sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0135): `scripts/hard_wall_kit.py`.
  Four sub-checks on finite-dimensional non-commuting matrix models: **A** resolvent
  non-idempotent at finite $\varepsilon$ + hard-wall recovery as $\varepsilon\kappa\to\infty$;
  **B** plain resolvent palindrome has non-zero $\tau^2$ (order-1 — primary obstruction);
  **B′** Cayley upgrade restores order-2 for a smooth rate (narrow path exists);
  **C** sharp-layer blow-up of $\|[L,\rho]\|$ and the $\tau^3$ constant (boundary-layer
  obstruction). MUST print `PREFLIGHT-HARD-WALL PASS` (exit 0) iff every sub-check
  gives its expected sign; the printed VERDICT is **NO-GO**. Integrated into the
  `test-fast` sympy sweep. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; CI-safe without
  `slow-tests`. This gate **passing documents the NO-GO** (mirrors the GO-documenting
  `verify_killing_order2_preflight.py` of §21.8).
- **`G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2`** is **NOT** declared `RELEASE_BLOCKING` by this spike (it
  would not pass — §44.bis.4). `properties.yaml` is UNCHANGED. ADR-0135 stays
  **PROPOSED** with a NO-GO amendment.

### §44.bis.7 — References (§44.bis)

- G. Barles, P. E. Souganidis, *Convergence of approximation schemes for fully nonlinear
  second order equations*, **Asymptotic Anal.** 4 (1991) 271–283. — monotone + stable +
  consistent $\Rightarrow$ convergence to the unique viscosity solution (§44.bis.2).
- S. D. Howison, C. Reisinger, J. H. Witte, *The Effect of Non-Smooth Payoffs on the
  Penalty Approximation of American Options*, **SIAM J. Financial Math.** 4 (2013)
  539–574. doi:10.1137/090776089. — penalty boundary-layer $\delta=\sigma\sqrt\varepsilon$,
  value error $O(1/\rho)$, Delta $O(\rho^{-1/2})$ — the soft-wall accuracy cap (§44.bis.4).

  — hard-killing order-1 cap; §5 higher-order conjecture (§21, §21.8).
