## §44.ter — F3 RE-SPIKE (INVENTIVE): order-2 hard absorbing wall via the Crank–Nicolson Cayley map of the killed Dirichlet generator — GO (v8.0.0, ADR-0135 Amendment 2, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> **Status: NORMATIVE. RULING: GO for a RELEASE_BLOCKING `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2`
> order-2 hard-wall self-convergence gate.** This section SUPERSEDES the §44.bis
> NO-GO *for the post-multiply construction only* — §44.bis remains a correct,
> NORMATIVE obstruction record for the resolvent-mask route `P_ε C(τ) P_ε`. The
> RE-SPIKE solves the *same contradiction C3* by a STRUCTURALLY DIFFERENT
> construction (the boundary lives in the generator's domain, not in a composed
> mask), reaching genuine global order-2. The sympy oracle
> `scripts/killed_generator_cn_kit.py` (`T_KILLED_GEN_CN`, sub-checks A/B/C/D)
> symbolically PROVES the order-2 claim. The ARIZ chain that produced this
> construction is recorded in `.dev-docs/research/F3_ARIZ_killed_generator_cn.md`.

### §44.ter.1 — The construction (NORMATIVE)

Let `L = ∂_x(a(x) ∂_x)` (+ optional drift/reaction) on the open absorbing region
`R = (x_L, x_R) ⊊ ℝ` with the hard wall `u|_{∂R} = 0` (barrier options, killed
Brownian motion, American/optimal-stopping continuation region). Define the
**killed Dirichlet generator** `L^R` as the discrete realization of `L` on the
INTERIOR grid nodes with the absorbing boundary condition baked into its DOMAIN:
the boundary nodes carry the fixed value `0` and contribute nothing to the
interior stencil (a boundary-neighbour term `a/dx²·u_∂` is replaced by `a/dx²·0`).
`L^R` is the standard symmetric-tridiagonal Dirichlet Laplacian; it is NOT a
free-space operator post-multiplied by a mask.

Step with the **Crank–Nicolson Cayley map** of `L^R`:
$$
U^{n+1} \;=\; \bigl(I - \tfrac{\tau}{2}\,L^R\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(I + \tfrac{\tau}{2}\,L^R\bigr)\,U^n,
\tag{44.ter.1}
$$
one implicit tridiagonal solve per step (scalar Thomas; the `M = 1` case of the
shipped `block_thomas_solve`, math §33 / `matrix_strang.rs`). The Dirichlet
boundary rows of the assembled matrix are the identity (`u_∂ ← u_∂`), so a datum
that is `0` on `∂R` stays `0` for all `τ` to machine precision.

### §44.ter.2 — Order-of-accuracy derivation (NORMATIVE)

**Theorem (order-2 hard wall, variable coefficients — NORMATIVE, ADR-0149).**
The τ²-cancellation that gives order-2 is the **pure matrix-algebra identity** (★):
$$
\bigl(I - \tfrac{\tau}{2}G\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(I + \tfrac{\tau}{2}G\bigr)
\;=\; e^{\tau G} \;+\; \tfrac{1}{12}\,\tau^3 G^3 \;+\; O(\tau^4),
\tag{★}
$$
which holds for **any fixed square matrix `G`** — the derivation uses only the binomial
expansion of the Neumann-series inverse and the power-series of `e^{τG}`, invoking no
structure of `G` beyond it being a fixed matrix. Applied to the killed Dirichlet
generator `L^R`:
- Variable `a(x), b(x)` change only the **numeric entries** of the tridiagonal `L^R`
  (off-diagonals become `a_{k±1/2}/dx²`, drift adds `b_k/(2dx)`), not the algebraic
  form of (★). Hence **`τ¹ = τ² = 0`** and the leading remainder is **`τ³·(L^R)³/12`**
  regardless of whether the coefficient field is constant or varies node-to-node.
- **Self-adjointness is NOT required** for the τ²-cancellation. (★) holds for every
  fixed matrix `G`, including non-symmetric (advection–diffusion) generators with
  non-zero drift `b(x)`. Self-adjointness of `L^R` is needed only for unconditional
  **A-stability** (spectral abscissa `≤ 0`); it is NOT needed for **order-2**.

The per-step local truncation error is therefore
$$
\bigl(I - \tfrac{\tau}{2}L^R\bigr)^{-1}\bigl(I + \tfrac{\tau}{2}L^R\bigr)
\;=\; e^{\tau L^R} \;+\; \tfrac{1}{12}\,\tau^3 (L^R)^3 \;+\; O(\tau^4),
\tag{44.ter.2}
$$
i.e. **`τ¹` and `τ²` terms vanish, the leading remainder is `O(τ³)`** ⟹ global
convergence order **2** in `τ` (Hochbruck–Lubich 2010 §3.4; Strang 1968). Because the
hard wall `u|_{∂R} = 0` is part of the generator `L^R` (not a separately-composed
operation), this order-2 IS the hard-wall order-2.

**Symbolic proof (oracle CHECK C of `scripts/killed_dirichlet_varcoef_kit.py`
= T_KILLED_GEN_CN CHECK E):** A fully symbolic `3×3` tridiagonal generator with
INDEPENDENT distinct symbolic entries `p1,p2,p3,l2,l3,u1,u2` (the most general
variable-coefficient killed stencil — no numeric specialisation) satisfies (★)
symbolically: `τ² ≡ 0` and the `τ³` residual `≡ G³/12` as a polynomial identity in
all 7 symbols. This makes GO **unambiguous**: variable `a(x)/b(x)` cannot break the
`τ²`-cancellation because (★) is an algebraic identity, not a constant-coefficient
accident. See `scripts/killed_dirichlet_varcoef_kit.py` (PREFLIGHT-KILLED-VARCOEF
PASS 6/6) and `scripts/killed_generator_cn_kit.py` CHECK E (T_KILLED_GEN_CN 5/5).

**The conditions** (precise): (i) `a(x) > 0` bounded (ellipticity — needed for the
tridiagonal to be non-singular and for A-stability of `L^R`); (ii) `b(x)` bounded
(drift finite — the generator is well-posed); (iii) the spatial discretization of
`L^R` is itself order-2 in `dx` (standard 3-point divergence-form stencil); (iv) the
absorbing datum is `0` on `∂R` (Dirichlet — the construction does NOT provide
Neumann/Robin, which are §25/§26.bis). Under (i)–(iv) the global order is **2**,
NOT higher: (44.ter.2) leaves a genuine `τ³` remainder (oracle CHECK A, CHECK E —
verified on a generic degree-6 non-origin-symmetric jet, ADR-0136 honesty discipline)
— no overclaim.

> **NARROW notes (unchanged — not removable).**
> 1. *A-stability requires self-adjointness*: for a non-self-adjoint `L^R`
>    (large drift `b(x)`), the CN map remains order-2 (CHECK F of
>    `killed_dirichlet_varcoef_kit.py`), but A-stability (spectral abscissa `≤ 0`) may
>    fail if `b` dominates `a`; in that case CN can be unstable for large `τ`. The
>    Rust gate uses a self-adjoint (`b=0`) kernel; non-self-adjoint coefficient
>    configurations are the user's responsibility.
> 2. *Non-smooth data / Rannacher startup*: the GLOBAL order-2 in `τ` requires the
>    initial datum to be compatible with `L^R` (smooth enough that `L^R f` is
>    bounded). For non-smooth data (e.g. discontinuous payoffs) the global rate may
>    degrade; Rannacher 1984 backward-Euler startup restores order-2 globally.
>    This is a DATA regularity issue, NOT a coefficient-variation order drop.
> 3. *Free-boundary cap*: the `O(√τ)` global rate for American/obstacle problems
>    (§44.ter.5) is a structural property of the free boundary, unchanged by this
>    theorem.

### §44.ter.3 — How C3a/C3b/C3c are RESOLVED, not relocated (NORMATIVE)

The §44.bis obstructions all stem from one root cause: the boundary was enforced as a
SEPARATE operation (mask `𝟙_R` or reaction rate `ρ`) composed with a DIFFERENT operator
(the free-space flow `C`). The RE-SPIKE removes that composition.

- **C3a (idempotency collapse).** GONE — there is no post-multiply mask `𝟙_R`; nothing
  is idempotent. The single operator `L^R` is a generator, and the Cayley map of any
  generator is order-2 unconditionally. Oracle CHECK A: `τ² = 0`.
- **C3b (factor accuracy `(I+τρ)^{-1/2}` vs `e^{-τρ/2}` only `O(τ)`).** GONE — there is
  no second factor. The (1,1)-Padé `(I−τL^R/2)^{-1}(I+τL^R/2)` matches `e^{τL^R}` to
  `O(τ³)` exactly (44.ter.2), which is precisely the Cayley upgrade §44.bis CHECK B′
  identified as the *only* order-2 path — applied here to the generator itself rather
  than to a bump rate. Oracle CHECK A.
- **C3c (boundary-layer commutator blow-up `‖[L,ρ]‖ ~ 1/dx²` under `ε = α·dx`).** GONE —
  there is no rate ramp `ρ` and no width parameter `ε` to sharpen. The wall is a DOMAIN
  RESTRICTION of width 0, exact at every `τ` (CHECK B). The leading `τ³` LTE constant is
  governed by the SMOOTH operator `(L^R)³` and stays bounded under refinement (oracle
  CHECK C: `‖τ³ const‖` is `5/24` at 3 interior nodes and `5/24` at 4 — no negative power
  of `dx`). The coupled `τ↔dx` self-convergence slope is the true `−2`, not the `≈ −1`
  flattening of §44.bis.4.

Thus contradiction **C3 is RESOLVED** (both properties held at once: sharp hard wall AND
global order-2), in contrast to §44.bis where it was merely RELOCATED. The IKR realized:
*the boundary enforces itself, for free, by being part of the operator, leaving the
order-2 untouched.*

### §44.ter.4 — Strict dominance over the shipped order-1 hard wall (NORMATIVE)

`KillingChernoff<C,R>` (§21.3, v2.6) is `𝟙_R · C(τ)` — a free-space flow post-masked —
and is order-1 globally (the `[L,𝟙_R]` commutator cap, §21.2; §21.8 proved the symmetric
upgrade vacuous over the idempotent indicator). On the SAME finite model the post-multiply
mask has interior `τ²` residual `[1/8, 0, 1/8] ≠ 0` (oracle CHECK D) while the killed-
generator Cayley map has `τ² = 0` (CHECK A). The RE-SPIKE kernel is therefore a STRICTLY
HIGHER-ORDER sibling of `KillingChernoff`, not a faster variant of the same operator. The
v2.6 `KillingChernoff` is UNCHANGED and remains the order-1 reference; the new kernel is
the order-2 vehicle for the same hard-wall problem.

### §44.ter.5 — Unification: the order-2 inner for American / obstacle free-boundary VIs (NORMATIVE, optional second gate)

The free-boundary American/optimal-stopping problem is the variational inequality
`min(−∂_t V + (−L)V, V − g) = 0` solved by `ObstacleChernoff` (§44) as
`V^{n+1} = Π_g(S(τ) V^n)`, `Π_g = max(·, g)`. Today `ObstacleChernoff` wraps an order-1
inner `S` (its declared `order() == 1`, §44.4). Composing the projection with the
**killed-generator Cayley inner** (44.ter.1) gives an order-2 inner in the CONTINUATION
region `{V > g}`, where the scheme is smooth; at the FREE BOUNDARY the projection caps the
*global* rate at `O(√τ)` for non-smooth payoffs (Howison–Reisinger–Witte 2013) — a
structural property of the obstacle, NOT a defect of the inner, and NOT removable by any
inner. Hence:

- **Hard-wall gate `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2`** (NORMATIVE, RELEASE_BLOCKING): a *fixed*-barrier
  problem (no obstacle) has a smooth continuation region; the killed-generator Cayley map
  delivers the FULL order-2 there. Self-convergence slope `≤ −1.95`.
- **Free-boundary note** (advisory, NOT a blocking order-2 gate): the American/obstacle
  composite improves the continuation-region accuracy to order-2 but its *global* free-
  boundary rate stays `O(√τ)`. A gate here would be a CONTINUATION-REGION (interior, away
  from contact) order-2 slope check, NOT a global free-boundary order-2 claim — declaring
  global order-2 at a free boundary would be an OVERCLAIM and is explicitly refused
  (honesty guardrail). v8.x MAY add an advisory `G_AMERICAN_CONTINUATION_ORDER2`.

### §44.ter.6 — Acceptance (`T_KILLED_GEN_CN` — NORMATIVE; `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` DECLARED)

- **`T_KILLED_GEN_CN` sympy gate** (NORMATIVE — ADR-0135 Am. 2 + ADR-0149):
  `scripts/killed_generator_cn_kit.py`. **Five** sub-checks on finite-dimensional matrix
  models: **A** the killed-generator Cayley map is order-2 (`τ¹ = τ² = 0`, `τ³ ≠ 0`
  vs `e^{τL^R}`, constant-`a` model); **B** the Dirichlet domain is preserved exactly
  (boundary rows = identity ∀τ — hard BC, no layer); **C** the `τ³` constant is bounded
  under refinement (no `1/dx` blow-up — C3c absent); **D** the v2.6 post-multiply mask has
  nonzero `τ²` (order-1) while the Cayley map has `τ² = 0` (order-2) — strict dominance;
  **E** *(added ADR-0149, v8.2.0)* variable-`a` honesty jet: the killed Dirichlet Cayley
  map of a STRICTLY VARIABLE-`a` generator applied to a generic degree-6
  non-origin-symmetric jet gives `τ¹ = τ² = 0` and genuinely nonzero `τ³` ⟹ order
  EXACTLY 2, not spuriously higher (ADR-0136 anti-over-report discipline). CHECK E
  confirms that CHECK A's τ²-cancellation is the matrix identity (★) and PERSISTS for
  variable coefficients — it is NOT a constant-`a` artifact. The companion script
  `scripts/killed_dirichlet_varcoef_kit.py` (PREFLIGHT-KILLED-VARCOEF 6/6) provides a
  deeper symbolic proof (CHECK C: fully symbolic tridiagonal, τ² ≡ 0 as a polynomial
  identity in 7 symbols). MUST print `PREFLIGHT-KILLED-GEN-CN PASS` (exit 0) iff every
  sub-check gives its expected sign; the printed VERDICT is **GO**. Integrated into the
  `test-fast` sympy sweep. Pure symbolic — no library runtime; CI-safe without
  `slow-tests`.
- **`G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2`** is **DECLARED** `RELEASE_BLOCKING` (`properties.yaml`): a hard-
  barrier self-convergence test, slope `≤ −1.95` over a grid sweep with `τ` coupled to `dx`
  at order-2 spatial accuracy. IC: `sin(x)` on `[0, π]` (Dirichlet mode-1 eigenfunction;
  NOT origin-symmetric in the polynomial sense; the gate measures SPATIAL order, not
  τ-order, so the ADR-0136 low-polynomial-degree concern is inapplicable — see
  §44.ter.6.1 below). Authority: ADR-0135 Amendment 2 + ADR-0149.

#### §44.ter.6.1 — `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` probe IC: `sin(x)` is an HONEST probe

ADR-0136 Amendment 1 established that **polynomial** / group-action probes where
`(L^R)^m P = 0` for the gate's leading remainder `m` spuriously make the τ³ residual
vanish, inflating the measured order. The `sin(x)` probe in `G_HARD_WALL_ORDER2` does
NOT suffer from this: (a) `sin(x)` is not a polynomial — the FD discretization of
`L^R sin = −a·sin` has a nonzero spatial truncation `O(dx²)` at every interior node;
(b) the gate measures **spatial** convergence (sweep over `n_spatial` at fixed `T` with
`τ = dx²`), not τ-order isolation — the measured slope `≈ −2.04` comes from the 3-point
FD stencil's eigenvalue bias `Δλ ≈ −dx²/12`, which is NOT suppressed by any
origin-symmetry or low polynomial degree of `sin`; (c) `sin(x)` is antisymmetric about
`x = π/2`, not origin-symmetric. The `sin(x)` probe is therefore HONEST for this spatial
convergence gate. No IC change required.

### §44.ter.7 — References (§44.ter)

- M. Hochbruck, C. Lubich, *Exponential integrators*, **Acta Numerica** 19 (2010) 209–286.
  §3.4 — the Cayley / (1,1)-Padé map is A-stable and order-2 unconditionally (44.ter.2).
- G. Strang, *On the construction and comparison of difference schemes*, **SIAM J. Numer.
  Anal.** 5:3 (1968) 506–517. — the order-2 palindrome that §44.bis showed the resolvent
  *mask* cannot match but the generator Cayley map DOES.
- S. D. Howison, C. Reisinger, J. H. Witte, **SIAM J. Financial Math.** 4 (2013) 539–574. —
  free-boundary `O(√τ)` cap for non-smooth American payoffs (§44.ter.5 honesty note).

  post-multiply killing functional that this RE-SPIKE supersedes structurally (§44.ter.4).

## §45 — Action-of-exponential `e^{τA}·v` via scaled truncated Taylor (Al-Mohy & Higham 2011 `expmv`) — `DiffusionExpmvChernoff` (v7.0, ADR-0121, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics)

> Scope: this section is the normative basis for the `DiffusionExpmvChernoff`
> kernel (`crates/semiflow-core/src/expmv.rs`). It is an ADDITIVE tolerance-driven
> ζ⁸-class propagator that REVIVES the ζ⁸-accuracy goal closed for the *operator-
> level Padé* kernel by ADR-0101 (§27.quart AMENDMENT 3), via a structurally
> different published algorithm. ADR-0101's Padé deferral is UNCHANGED — this is a
> different kernel class, not a fourth Padé attempt.

### §45.1 — Algorithm (NORMATIVE)

For the divergence-form generator $A = \partial_x(a(x)\,\partial_x)\,(+\,b\,\partial_x + c)$
discretised by the 3-point Neumann stencil `apply_div_form` (§40.7), the action
$e^{\tau A} v$ is computed WITHOUT forming, squaring, or inverting any matrix, by
applying a truncated Taylor polynomial $T_m(\tau A / s)$ to the VECTOR, $s$ times:

$$
e^{\tau A} v = \bigl(e^{(\tau/s) A}\bigr)^{s} v \approx \bigl(T_m(\tfrac{\tau}{s} A)\bigr)^{s} v,
\qquad T_m(z) = \sum_{k=0}^{m} \frac{z^k}{k!}.
$$

Realised as Horner-on-vector (one banded mat-vec per inner term):

```
y ← v
for i in 1..=s:
    w ← y
    for k in 1..=m:
        w ← (τ/s) · (A·w) / k       # one apply_div_form
        y ← y + w
return y                             # ≈ e^{τA} v
```

The scaling parameter $s = \lceil \tau\,\lVert A\rVert / \theta_m \rceil$ bounds each
per-application argument $(\tau/s)\lVert A\rVert \le \theta_m$ below the degree-$m$
backward-error radius $\theta_m$ (Al-Mohy & Higham 2011 Table 3.1). With the
crate's conservative analytic bound $\lVert A\rVert_{\mathrm{est}} \approx 4\,a_\infty/\mathrm{d}x^2$,
over-estimation only RAISES $s$ (more, cheaper steps) without harming accuracy.
The degree is capped at $M_{\max} = 18$ (a plain monomial Horner above
$\arg \approx 9$ loses precision; remaining argument is traded into $s$ — Al-Mohy &
Higham Code Fragment 3.1 guard). Total cost: $s\cdot m$ banded mat-vecs, each
$O(K\!\cdot\!N)$; no LU, no $Q^{-1}$, no dense matrix; $O(1)$ work vectors $y, w$
($\texttt{no\_std + alloc}$ clean).

### §45.2 — Why this is NOT the closed Padé path (structural bypass; CITATION)

ADR-0101 (§27.quart AMENDMENT 3) terminally deferred the operator-level Padé kernel
$Q_4(\tau_s A)^{-1} P_4(\tau_s A)$ on three failure modes — D1 (P₄/Q₄ coefficient
transcription), D2 (banded-LU error propagation under squaring), and the envelope
blow-up $\tau\lVert A\rVert \approx 62 \gg \theta_4 = 5.4$ — and made revival
conditional on a *published* algorithm bypassing the Wave-I bug at the
algorithmic-equivalence level. `expmv` satisfies this STRUCTURALLY:

1. **No rational branch** — $T_m$ is a polynomial: there is no $Q_4$ to transcribe
   (D1 cannot exist) and no banded-LU solve (D2 cannot exist).
2. **No matrix squaring** — the ADR-0101 "$R^{2^s}\!\cdot v \equiv R\cdots R\cdot v$"
   equivalence (which falsified D3) is moot: there is no fixed rational $R$. The full
   step is recovered by repeated *polynomial* application on the vector.
3. **`s`-scaling tames the blow-up** — choosing $s = \lceil\tau\lVert A\rVert/\theta_m\rceil$
   makes each application see argument $< \theta_m$ by construction; the
   $\tau\lVert A\rVert\approx 62$ regime that diverged the Padé kernel is exactly the
   regime $s$-scaling is designed for.

### §45.3 — PRE-FLIGHT clearance (sympy/numpy; CITATION)

PRE-FLIGHT harness `scripts/verify_expmv_preflight.py` (executed 2026-06-05) on a
banded divergence-form $A$ (N=64, $a(x)=1+0.3\sin(2\pi x/L)$, $\tau\lVert A\rVert_1 = 62.00$):
(a) the scaled action reaches $\texttt{sup\_error} = 1.1\times 10^{-15}$ with every
per-step argument $\le \theta_m$; (b) raising the truncation degree at fixed $s$ gives
super-algebraic convergence ($\log_2$ ratios $+10.77, +10.67, +10.50$) from
$8.3\times 10^{-5}$ to round-off — the OPPOSITE of Wave-I's persistent
$\log_2 = -0.4053$ anti-convergence; (c) the Algorithm 3.2 auto-selected $(s{=}8,m{=}18)$
gives $1.1\times 10^{-15}$ and SciPy's independent `expm_multiply` gives
$1.4\times 10^{-15}$ — both $\approx 3700\times$ below the Chebyshev ζ⁸ effective floor
$4.17\times 10^{-12}$ (§27.tris / `diffusion8_zeta8.rs`). All three sub-checks PASS → GO.

### §45.4 — Gate (NORMATIVE)

`g_expmv_div_form_action_accuracy` (`slow-tests`-gated): backward-error gate, NOT a
fixed-order slope (`expmv` is tolerance-driven, so the §27/§40 "slope $\le -K$" pattern
is INAPPLICABLE). Compare against a high-$s$ self-converged reference (mirror the
`G_zeta8` self-convergence pattern, §27.tris); assert $\texttt{sup\_error} \le 10^{-11}$
(one order above the Chebyshev floor for discretisation headroom).

**References (§45)**:
- A. H. Al-Mohy and N. J. Higham, *Computing the Action of the Matrix Exponential, with an Application to Exponential Integrators*, **SIAM J. Sci. Comput.** 33(2):488–511, 2011. DOI 10.1137/100788860 — primary (`expmv`, action form, Table 3.1 $\theta_m$, Algorithm 3.2).
- A. H. Al-Mohy and N. J. Higham, *A New Scaling and Squaring Algorithm for the Matrix Exponential*, **SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl.** 31(3):970–989, 2009/2010. DOI 10.1137/09074721X — backward-error machinery ($\alpha_p$, $\theta_m$).
- ADR-0121 (revives ζ⁸ goal via `expmv`; supersedes ADR-0101 closure with the published bypass it required); ADR-0101 / §27.quart AMENDMENT 3 (Padé operator-level kernel TERMINAL CLOSURE — UNCHANGED); ADR-0090 / §27.tris (Chebyshev `Diffusion8thZeta8Chernoff` — additive sibling + cross-validation target); ADR-0118 / §40.7 (`apply_div_form` $A\cdot v$ primitive).

## §46 — Forward-mode dual-number AD over the Chernoff product structure — `Dual<F>` (v8.0.0 HEADLINE, ADR-0133, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics — second S-curve)

> Scope: this section is the normative basis for the `Dual<F>` scalar field
> (`crates/semiflow-core/src/dual.rs`) and its blanket participation as the field
> parameter of `ChernoffFunction<Dual<F>>`. It is STRICTLY ADDITIVE: no existing
> kernel's semantics, signature, or numerical output for `F ∈ {f32, f64}` changes.
> `Dual<F>` is a NEW member of the `SemiflowFloat` family (it satisfies every
> `SemiflowFloat` supertrait bound); instantiating any generic kernel at
> `F = Dual<f64>` yields forward-mode automatic differentiation of that kernel's
> output with respect to one scalar parameter `θ`, at ZERO new heap allocation.
> The new S-curve axis (ADR-0132) is the previously-unused **product structure**
> `(F(τ))ⁿ`; this section differentiates it.

### §46.1 — The dual field (NORMATIVE)

A **dual number** over a base scalar field $F$ is the pair

$$
\mathrm{Dual}(a, b) \;=\; a + \varepsilon\, b, \qquad a,b \in F, \qquad \varepsilon^2 = 0,
$$

with the nilpotent unit $\varepsilon$ (NOT the imaginary unit: $\varepsilon^2 = 0$,
whereas $i^2 = -1$). The first component $a$ is the **value**; the second component
$b$ is the **tangent**. The algebra $F[\varepsilon]/(\varepsilon^2)$ is commutative
and associative. Seeding the tangent of a parameter $\theta$ with $1$ — i.e.
evaluating a computation on $\mathrm{Dual}(\theta_0, 1)$ — makes the tangent of the
result equal to the exact derivative of the result's value with respect to
$\theta$, evaluated at $\theta_0$. This is forward-mode AD with one independent
direction.

### §46.2 — Dual arithmetic and the chain rule (NORMATIVE)

Let $U = \mathrm{Dual}(u, u')$ and $V = \mathrm{Dual}(v, v')$, where $'$ denotes
$\mathrm{d}/\mathrm{d}\theta$. Truncating every product at $\varepsilon^2 = 0$ yields
the field operations (these are the EXACT rules `impl` must reproduce):

$$
\begin{aligned}
U + V &= \mathrm{Dual}\!\bigl(u+v,\; u'+v'\bigr), &
U - V &= \mathrm{Dual}\!\bigl(u-v,\; u'-v'\bigr), \\[2pt]
U \cdot V &= \mathrm{Dual}\!\bigl(uv,\; u'v + u v'\bigr) \;\text{(product rule)}, &
U / V &= \mathrm{Dual}\!\Bigl(\tfrac{u}{v},\; \tfrac{u'v - u v'}{v^2}\Bigr) \;\text{(quotient rule)}.
\end{aligned}
$$

For any differentiable scalar function $g$ required by the `SemiflowFloat : Float`
bound, the action on a dual is the **chain rule**:

$$
g\bigl(\mathrm{Dual}(u, u')\bigr) \;=\; \mathrm{Dual}\!\bigl(g(u),\; g'(u)\,u'\bigr).
$$

The transcendental and structural ops the kernels actually call — and their NORMATIVE
tangent rules — are:

| op | value | tangent $g'(u)\,u'$ |
|----|-------|---------------------|
| `exp`  | $e^{u}$        | $e^{u}\,u'$ |
| `ln`   | $\ln u$        | $u'/u$ |
| `sqrt` | $\sqrt{u}$     | $u' / (2\sqrt{u})$ |
| `recip`| $1/u$          | $-u'/u^2$ |
| `sin`  | $\sin u$       | $\cos(u)\,u'$ |
| `cos`  | $\cos u$       | $-\sin(u)\,u'$ |
| `powi(n)` | $u^{n}$     | $n\,u^{n-1}\,u'$ |
| `abs`  | $\lvert u\rvert$ | $\operatorname{sgn}(u)\,u'$ (sub-gradient $0$ at $u=0$) |

`powf`, `tanh`, `floor`, comparisons, `is_finite`, etc. follow the same template
(`floor`/comparisons act on the value; tangent of a piecewise-constant op is $0$).
Ordering (`PartialOrd`) and equality compare **value components only** — the tangent
is carried, never compared — so validation guards (`tau < 0`, `a(x) < 0`) behave
identically to the scalar path.

### §46.3 — Why this rides in the product structure at zero new allocation (NORMATIVE + CITATION)

The Chernoff approximant is the $n$-fold product $\bigl(F(\tau)\bigr)^{n}$ (Chernoff
1968; Theorem 6, §5). Differentiating it with respect to a parameter $\theta$ in
$F$ gives, by the product rule,

$$
\frac{\mathrm d}{\mathrm d\theta}\bigl(F(\tau)\bigr)^{n}
\;=\; \sum_{j=1}^{n} \bigl(F(\tau)\bigr)^{j-1}\,\frac{\mathrm dF(\tau)}{\mathrm d\theta}\,\bigl(F(\tau)\bigr)^{n-j},
$$

a sum of $n$ products each with **exactly one factor replaced by**
$\mathrm dF/\mathrm d\theta$. This is precisely what dual arithmetic computes
automatically: running the existing $n$-step ping-pong iteration (chernoff.rs
`Evolver::evolve_into`) with the scalar field replaced by $\mathrm{Dual}(F\text{-value}, F\text{-derivative})$
advances value and derivative **in the same loop pass, in the same registers**. No
tape is recorded; no per-step heap node is allocated; the derivative occupies the
tangent slot of the same `State<Dual<F>>` buffer that already exists. The
steady-state allocation count per `evolve()` is therefore IDENTICAL to the
$F = \texttt{f64}$ baseline (gate `G_DUAL_ZERO_ALLOC`). This is the ВПР of the
second S-curve: the product structure was always there; the dual field harvests its
derivative for free.

### §46.4 — Hyper-dual path for second derivatives Γ (NORMATIVE)

Second derivatives (Γ-Greeks; the Hessian diagonal of an ML loss through the kernel)
are obtained by NESTING the field: $\mathrm{Dual}\langle\mathrm{Dual}\langle F\rangle\rangle$.
Because `Dual<Dual<F>>` again satisfies every `SemiflowFloat` bound (the construction is
closed under nesting), it rides the SAME blanket `ChernoffFunction<Dual<Dual<F>>>` with
no additional kernel code. Seeding both inner and outer tangents with $1$ on the target
parameter makes the $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$ cross-component of the result equal to
the exact $\mathrm d^2/\mathrm d\theta^2$ of the output value. Cost is constant-factor
(four-wide field instead of two-wide); allocation count is still unchanged versus
baseline (the buffer element is wider, the buffer COUNT is identical).

### §46.5 — SIMD fall-through (NORMATIVE; ADR-0018 carve-out preserved)

The AVX2/NEON specialisations (Catmull-Rom, K-kernel, `Strang2D/3D` parallel paths)
remain `f64`-ONLY per ADR-0018 — they are unaffected and unchanged. `Dual<F>` does NOT
implement the SIMD intrinsic paths; a kernel instantiated at `F = Dual<f64>` falls
through to the scalar Rust ops (the generic `default` code path that already backs
`f32`). This is acceptable BY DESIGN: AD is a calibration / sensitivity workload
(Jacobians, training gradients), not the 45 ns L1d-resident hot loop. The
`STRANG2D_PARALLEL_BIT_EQUAL` and `diffusion4_unit` SIMD regressions (constitution
Principle 3) are untouched because no `Dual` path enters them.

### §46.5.bis — Interpolation-order coverage of the AD path (NORMATIVE)

The forward-mode AD path runs every kernel at `F = Dual<f64>` through the
**generic scalar sampler** `GridFn1D::sample_generic → Grid1D::interp_generic`
(grid_fn.rs / grid.rs), NOT the `f64`-specialised `sample → interp` path. The
two dispatch tables are NOT identical, and this section pins which `InterpKind`
variants the AD path composes with.

The `f64` path `Grid1D::interp` supports the full ladder: `CubicHermite`,
`SepticHermite` (the v6.0+ **default** of `Grid1D::new`, ADR-0109 / §40),
`OctonicHermite` (ADR-0117 / §41), and `ChebyshevSpectralWithBC` (§9.2.bis).
Before v8.0.0, the generic path `interp_generic` supported only `CubicHermite`
and (feature-gated) `Linear`; the three high-order variants returned
`SemiflowError::Unsupported`. Because `Grid1D::new` defaults to `SepticHermite`
since v6.0, a user who built a grid with the default sampler and instantiated a
kernel at `F = Dual<f64>` received `Unsupported` — AD silently did not compose
with the **default** grid. v8.0.0 (ADR-0133) added `SepticHermite` to the
generic path, closing that default-grid gap. v8.1.0 (ADR-0139) completed the
ladder by adding `OctonicHermite` (via `octonic_generic.rs`) and
`ChebyshevSpectralWithBC` (via `chebyshev_generic.rs`).

**NORMATIVE (v8.0.0):** the generic sampler MUST support `SepticHermite` so that
the AD path composes with the **default** `Grid1D::new` grid. The septic-Hermite
interpolant of §40 is a finite sum of degree-≤7 polynomials in the cell-local
coordinate `s` (closed-form weights `a0..a3, b0..b3`, all in `+,−,×` of `s`) acting
on nodal values and central-FD-reconstructed scaled derivatives `dx·f', dx²·f'',
dx³·f'''` (rational-constant stencils, §40.2). Every operation is a `SemiflowFloat`
field op for which `Dual<F>` carries the exact chain rule (§46.2); the genericised
sampler is therefore the **same closed form** with `f64` literals replaced by
`F::from(·)` and `bc_value → bc_value_generic`, and it differentiates correctly by
construction. No SIMD path participates (§46.5).

**NORMATIVE (v8.1.0 / ADR-0139):** `OctonicHermite` (§41) and
`ChebyshevSpectralWithBC` (§9.2.bis) are now fully supported on the generic AD
path. Kernels whose grid opts into either variant via `.with_interp(...)` compose
with `F = Dual<f64>` correctly; `SemiflowError::Unsupported` is no longer returned
for these two samplers.

*OctonicHermite* (`octonic_generic.rs`): the degree-≤9 Hermite interpolant of §41
is a closed-form polynomial in the cell-local coordinate `s` acting on nodal values
and scaled derivatives; every operation is a `SemiflowFloat` field op for which
`Dual<F>` carries the exact chain rule (§46.2), with `f64` literals promoted via
`F::from(·)`. No SIMD path participates (§46.5). Gate: generic-vs-scalar f64
agreement ≤32 ULP (measured 24 ULP); Dual-AD gradient |diff| vs Richardson FD
~1 × 10⁻¹⁴ (gate 1 × 10⁻⁹, PASS).

*ChebyshevSpectralWithBC* (`chebyshev_generic.rs`): the data-independent node/weight
tables (`chebyshev_nodes`, `chebyshev_weights`) are promoted entry-by-entry via
`F::from(table_entry)`; the subsequent barycentric-Lagrange reduction is purely
field-op-arithmetic (`+,×,÷` on `F` values) so `Dual<F>` carries the exact chain
rule at every step. No SIMD path participates (§46.5). Gate: generic-vs-scalar f64
agreement 0 ULP; Dual-AD gradient |diff| vs Richardson FD ~1 × 10⁻¹⁴ (gate
1 × 10⁻⁹, PASS).

**Coverage statement (v8.1.0, ADR-0139).** Forward-mode AD
composes with every kernel in the library at the *kernel* level (the blanket
`ChernoffFunction<Dual<F>>` is universal). As of v8.1.0 (ADR-0139), the
*interpolation* axis is no longer a non-universal seam: AD covers the **full
interpolation ladder** — `CubicHermite`, `SepticHermite` (§40, default),
`OctonicHermite` (§41), and `ChebyshevSpectralWithBC` (§9.2.bis). The ADR-0133
"all 25+ kernels" claim now holds for every shipped `InterpKind`, not only the
default grid.

### §46.6 — PRE-FLIGHT clearance (sympy; CITATION)

PRE-FLIGHT oracle `scripts/dual_ad_kit.py` (gate **T_DUAL**, executed 2026-06-07,
PASS 4/4) symbolically certifies, before any Rust is written: (a) `arithmetic` —
the $+,-,\times,\div$ tangents equal the sympy-exact derivative of the value
(product/quotient rules); (b) `transcendental` — the eight chain-rule ops of §46.2
match `sympy.diff` exactly; (c) `hyperdual_second_deriv` — the nested-dual
$\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$ component recovers $\mathrm d^2/\mathrm d\theta^2$
exactly for $g = \exp$; (d) `kernel_forward_grad` — the ζ-A symbol factor
$k(\theta) = e^{-\theta s^2}(1 + \theta s^2)$ differentiated in dual arithmetic
equals the symbolic exact gradient AND agrees with a central-difference probe to
$\le 10^{-10}$ (mirroring the `G_DUAL_AD_GRADIENT` acceptance comparison). All four
PASS → GO for engineer implementation.

### §46.7 — Gates (NORMATIVE)

- **`G_DUAL_AD_GRADIENT`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`): for a representative
  kernel set (at minimum `DiffusionChernoff`, `Diffusion4thChernoff`, `StrangSplit`),
  the forward-mode gradient $\partial_\theta\,(\text{evolved output})$ obtained by
  instantiating the kernel at `F = Dual<f64>` and seeding the parameter tangent with
  $1$ MUST match a central finite-difference gradient
  $\bigl(u(\theta_0+h) - u(\theta_0-h)\bigr)/(2h)$ to sup-norm tolerance
  $\le 10^{-10}$, at a step $h$ in the central-difference sweet spot. **At least one
  kernel in the set MUST run on a grid built by the default `Grid1D::new`
  constructor (i.e. `InterpKind::SepticHermite`, §46.5.bis) — NOT pinned to
  `CubicHermite` — so the gate exercises the genericised default spatial
  interpolant and would FAIL if the AD path silently fell back to `Unsupported`
  on the default grid.** A second sub-gate MAY pin `CubicHermite` for the
  cross-check against the pre-v8 path.
- **`G_DUAL_ZERO_ALLOC`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`): the steady-state heap
  allocation count of one `Evolver::evolve_into` call at `F = Dual<f64>` MUST equal
  the count at `F = f64` (measured by a counting global allocator over a warmed run;
  pre-warm excluded). Proves the "derivative for free" claim of §46.3.

**References (§46)**:
- P. H. Chernoff, *Note on product formulas for operator semigroups*, **J. Funct. Anal.** 2(2):238–242, 1968. DOI [10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7](https://doi.org/10.1016/0022-1236(68)90020-7) — the product structure $(S(t/n))^n$ being differentiated.
- W. Squire and G. Trapp, *Using complex variables to estimate derivatives of real functions*, **SIAM Review** 40(1):110–112, 1998 — forward-mode AD via a nilpotent/complex-step augmentation (the dual is the $\varepsilon^2=0$ analogue of the complex step, exact rather than $O(h^2)$).
- M. Fike and J. Alonso, *The Development of Hyper-Dual Numbers for Exact Second-Derivative Calculations*, AIAA 2011-886 — hyper-dual `Dual<Dual<F>>` second-derivative construction (§46.4).
- ADR-0133 (F1 dual-number forward AD over the Chernoff product structure); ADR-0132 (v8.0.0 umbrella — second S-curve / product-structure axis); ADR-0025/0026 (Generic-over-Float `SemiflowFloat` family that `Dual<F>` joins); ADR-0018 (SIMD `f64`-only carve-out preserved, §46.5); ADR-0041 (zero-alloc ping-pong `evolve_into` reused unchanged).

---

## §47 — Resolvent time-jump amortization via numerical Laplace inversion — `ResolventJumpChernoff` (v8.0.0 RESEARCH-TRACK, ADR-0134, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics — second S-curve)

### §47.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

Long horizons `T` and steady-state / implicit-grade targets require `n = T/τ → ∞` Chernoff steps, each `O(N)`, so total work is `O(T·N/τ)`. Pushing `τ` large enters the `‖A‖·τ ≳ 1` regime where the short-time Chernoff tangent degrades. The escape from §22 (ADR-0069) is that the resolvent `R(λ;A) = (λI − A)⁻¹` has norm `‖R(λ;A)‖ ≤ 1/(\operatorname{Re}λ − ω)`, **independent of `‖A‖`** — the `1/dx² → ∞` ceiling that PERMANENTLY blocks operator-Padé-in-time (ADR-0094, ADR-0101) disappears under the coordinate change to the spectral domain. This section ships a single LARGE time-step `e^{tA}g` as a **contour quadrature over bounded resolvent evaluations**, at a node count `M` that is **independent of `t`**.

### §47.2 — Cauchy / inverse-Laplace representation (CITATION — Trefethen–Weideman–Schmelzer 2006)

For a sectorial generator `A` (here self-adjoint, negative-semidefinite, growth bound `ω = 0`, spectrum `σ(A) ⊂ (−∞, 0]`), the semigroup admits the Bromwich / Cauchy integral
$$
e^{tA}\,g \;=\; \frac{1}{2\pi i} \oint_\Gamma e^{\lambda t}\,(\lambda I - A)^{-1}\,g\,\mathrm{d}\lambda, \tag{47.1}
$$
where `Γ` is a contour in the resolvent set `ρ(A)` winding once counter-clockwise around `σ(A)`. For a sectorial `A`, `Γ` is **deformed off the vertical Bromwich line into the left half-plane** to wrap the negative-real spectrum; this deformation is what converts the slowly-converging oscillatory Bromwich integral into a **geometrically (super-algebraically) convergent** quadrature. The optimised **parabolic contour** (Trefethen–Weideman–Schmelzer 2006, §3) is
$$
\lambda(\theta) \;=\; \frac{M}{t}\,\bigl(a_0 - a_1\,\theta^2 + i\,a_2\,\theta\bigr),
\qquad \theta \in (-\pi, \pi),
\qquad (a_0, a_1, a_2) = (0.1309,\, 0.1194,\, 0.2500). \tag{47.2}
$$
**The `M/t` scaling is the cost-decoupling mechanism**: substituting `λ = (M/t)·ζ` makes the integrand `e^{λ t} = e^{M ζ}` depend on `t` only through the contour scale, so the *number of nodes* needed for a target accuracy is `t`-INDEPENDENT (PRE-FLIGHT §47.6 sub-check 2: err-vs-`M` curves at `t ∈ {1, 20, 100}` coincide within `1.83×`). Discretising (47.1) with the midpoint rule on `M` equispaced angles `θ_k = −π + (k+½)(2π/M)`:
$$
e^{tA}\,g \;\approx\; \frac{1}{2\pi i}\sum_{k=0}^{M-1} e^{\lambda_k t}\,(\lambda_k I - A)^{-1}g\,\cdot\,\lambda'(\theta_k)\,\cdot\,\frac{2\pi}{M},
\qquad \lambda'(\theta) = \frac{M}{t}\bigl(-2a_1\theta + i\,a_2\bigr). \tag{47.3}
$$

**Theorem 47.1 (TWS 2006, geometric convergence).** For `A` sectorial with spectrum in a sector of half-angle `< π/2` about `(−∞, 0]`, the midpoint quadrature (47.3) on the parabolic contour (47.2) converges **geometrically**: `‖e^{tA}g − (47.3)‖ ≤ C·ρ^{M}` with `ρ < 1` and `C` independent of `t`. Empirically (§47.6) the decay is `−0.442` decades/node, reaching the `f64` floor at `M ≈ 28`.

### §47.3 — Cost decoupling and the per-node resolvent (NORMATIVE library)

The per-node operation in (47.3) is **one resolvent application** `(λ_k I − A)⁻¹ g` — exactly the object §22 ships. The cost of the entire large-`t` jump is therefore `M` resolvent solves with `M = O(1)` (typically `16–32`) **independent of `t`**, versus `n = T·‖A‖` Chernoff steps for the same horizon. This is the formal sense in which large-`T` cost is decoupled from the step ladder. The TRIZ resolution (ADR-0134): TRIZ-13 (inversion — substitute the temporal product expansion with a spectral one) + TRIZ-28 (field substitution — temporal → Laplace domain) where the resolvent is `‖A‖`-bounded; no infinite-norm matrix is ever squared (the ADR-0101 operator-Padé deferral is UNCHANGED — this is a coordinate change, not scaling-and-squaring).

### §47.4 — REUSE boundary and the LEFT-half-plane restriction (NORMATIVE library — NARROW)

The resolvent **abstraction** `(λI − A)⁻¹g` is reused from §22 / ADR-0069. **The shipped Gauss-Laguerre Laplace-Chernoff *quadrature* (`LaplaceChernoffResolvent::eval` / `eval_complex`, §22.6 + §22.9) is NOT a valid backend for the contour nodes.** Reason: the optimal contour (47.2) places **most nodes in the LEFT half-plane** `Re λ_k < 0` (PRE-FLIGHT §47.6 sub-check 4: `16/24` nodes have `Re λ ≤ 0` at `t = 20, M = 24`), but the Laplace integral representation `R̃_n(λ) = (1/λ)Σ w_k (C(s_k/(λn)))^n g` underlying `eval`/`eval_complex` is the Laplace transform `∫₀^∞ e^{−λt}S(t)g\,dt`, which **DIVERGES for `Re λ ≤ ω`** (§22.9 SPEC TRAP — the validity boundary is `Re λ > ω`, NOT `|λ| > ω`). A right-half-plane-confined contour does NOT recover this: shifting `Γ` into `Re λ > 0` makes `e^{λt}` grow without bound for large `t` and destroys the quadrature (PRE-FLIGHT: shifted-RHP contour err `≥ 5.3` at `σ₀ = 1.5`, `≥ 10¹³` at `σ₀ = 3`).

**NORMATIVE consequence.** `ResolventJumpChernoff` MUST evaluate `(λ_k I − A)⁻¹ g` with a **left-half-plane-capable resolvent backend** — a direct complex linear solve. For the divergence-form 1D Laplacian the discrete `(λI − A)` is **complex tridiagonal**, so a **complex Thomas solve is `O(N)` exact** (no iterative conditioning concern; `λ_k ∉ σ(A)` is guaranteed because the parabolic contour stays strictly off the negative-real axis). This LHP backend is the ONLY new numerical primitive; the contour loop, the TWS coefficients, and the weight assembly are pure scalar arithmetic. The restriction is **NARROW but benign for this library**: every diffusion / divergence-form generator shipped is self-adjoint negative-(semi)definite, so the sectorial hypothesis of Theorem 47.1 holds for the entire diffusion family (`DiffusionChernoff`, `Diffusion4thChernoff`, variable-`a` divergence form §40.7, anisotropic non-separable §10.7-ter). Non-self-adjoint / non-sectorial generators (large advection-dominated drift, expansive `ω ≫ 0`) are OUT of scope for v8.0.0 and MUST be rejected at construction or documented as caller responsibility.

### §47.5 — Acceptance gates (G_RESOLVENT_JUMP_ORDER + T_RESOLVENT_JUMP — NORMATIVE)

- **`G_RESOLVENT_JUMP_ORDER`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING — ADR-0134, `slow-tests`): Test operator `A = ∂_{xx}` on `L²([−5,5])` with `Reflect` boundary, `N = 64`, Gaussian datum `g(x) = e^{−x²}`, large horizon `t = 100`. Sweep `M ∈ {6, 8, 10, 12, 14}` parabolic contour nodes; reference is a many-small-step Chernoff (or exact `expm`) evaluation of `e^{tA}g`. The empirical `log`-`log` OLS slope `d log‖jump_M − ref‖_∞ / d log(1/M)` MUST be `≥ 1.95` (G24 convention: positive = order; the gate certifies at-least-order-2 effective convergence in the step `1/M`). Because the contour is geometrically convergent the measured slope is `≫ 1.95` (PRE-FLIGHT: `+9.86`), giving a large stability margin against grid / `λ`-placement perturbation. **Sign convention (NORMATIVE, mirrors G24 §22.5):** the slope is taken with respect to `log(1/M)`; a value `≥ +1.95` PASSES. (ADR-0134's prose "slope ≤ −1.95 in Δτ" is the same statement with the improvement-direction sign on `Δτ = 1/M`; the gate test MUST use the `≥ +1.95`-vs-`log(1/M)` form to match the shipped G24 harness and avoid a sign trap.)

- **`T_RESOLVENT_JUMP`** (NORMATIVE numeric+sympy oracle — ADR-0134, `scripts/resolvent_jump_kit.py`): 4 sub-checks, all mandatory; prints exactly `T_RESOLVENT_JUMP PASS` on success or `T_RESOLVENT_JUMP FAIL` on failure. (1) **geometric_decay** — `log10(err)` vs `M` is linear with rate `≤ −0.3` decades/node at `t = 20`. (2) **t_independence** — the `M = 16` error at `t ∈ {1, 20, 100}` spreads `≤ 10×` (cost decoupling). (3) **order_slope** — the G24-convention slope at `t = 100` is `≥ 1.95`. (4) **lhp_guard** — the optimal contour DOES place nodes in `Re λ < 0`, confirming the §47.4 NARROW restriction that `eval_complex` cannot be the backend. PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-06-07: **4/4 PASS** (rate `−0.442` dec/node; spread `1.83×`; slope `+9.86`; `16/24` nodes in the LHP). Integrated into the `test-fast` sympy sweep alongside `verify_complex_resolvent.py` (T_CPLX_RES) and `verify_resolvent_laplace_chernoff.py` (T19N). Failure BLOCKS v8.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity lesson.

### §47.6 — Limitations and future work

- **Self-adjoint / sectorial only (NARROW).** Theorem 47.1 requires `A` sectorial with spectrum in a sector `< π/2` about `(−∞, 0]`. True for all shipped diffusion / divergence-form generators (self-adjoint negative-semidefinite). Non-self-adjoint or advection-dominated (`ω ≫ 0`) generators are deferred to v8.x with a *hyperbolic* contour (TWS 2006 §4) and an adaptive-pole rational-Krylov backend.
- **Tridiagonal / banded `A` for the `O(N)` LHP solve.** The `O(N)` cost claim assumes a banded `(λI − A)` (true for the 3-pt and divergence-form 1D stencils). Higher-dimensional tensor / non-separable operators need a banded-block or sparse-`LU` LHP solve; the contour scheme is unchanged but per-node cost rises — defer the 2D/3D LHP backend to v8.x.
- **Fixed `(M, contour)`, no per-call adaptivity.** The user picks `M` and the parabolic contour at construction; runtime `t` only rescales the contour. An adaptive `M` driven by a residual estimate, and the hyperbolic-contour variant for stiffer sectors, are deferred (mirrors the §22.7 "no per-call adaptivity" deferral).
- **The contour backend bypasses the GL₃₂ Laplace-Chernoff path** (§47.4). This is intentional, not a defect: the two backends serve disjoint half-planes (`eval_complex` for `Re λ > ω` spectral analysis; `ResolventJumpChernoff` for the LHP Bromwich contour). They share only the resolvent *concept*.

### §47.7 — References

- L. N. Trefethen, J. A. C. Weideman, T. Schmelzer, *Talbot quadratures and rational approximations*, **BIT Numer. Math.** 46:3 (2006), pp. 653–670. — Optimised parabolic / hyperbolic contours for `e^{tA}` via numerical inverse Laplace transform; the `(a_0, a_1, a_2)` coefficients and geometric-convergence theorem of §47.2.
- A. Talbot, *The accurate numerical inversion of Laplace transforms*, **J. Inst. Math. Appl.** 23:1 (1979), pp. 97–120. — Foundational deformed-contour Bromwich inversion.
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 3. — The resolvent abstraction `(λI − A)⁻¹` reused here (via §22, ADR-0069).
- A. Pazy, *Semigroups of Linear Operators …*, Springer (1983), §1.5 — sectoriality and the resolvent set on the deformed contour.
- ADR-0134 (F2 resolvent time-jump amortization); ADR-0069 / math §22 (Laplace-Chernoff resolvent — abstraction reused); ADR-0127 / math §22.9 (complex-λ `eval_complex` — the `Re λ > ω` backend that is NOT valid on this contour); ADR-0101 / ADR-0094 (operator-Padé-in-time PERMANENT deferral — UNCHANGED; this is a coordinate change, not scaling-and-squaring).

### §47.8 — 2D/3D parabolic backends — `ResolventJumpChernoff2D` / `ResolventJumpChernoff3D` (v8.2.0, ADR-0148, NARROW-PARABOLIC)

**Context.** §47.6 deferred two extensions. This subsection ships bullet (b): the 2D/3D parabolic extension. Bullet (a), the **hyperbolic contour** for non-sectorial generators, remains **honestly deferred** per ADR-0148 Part B falsification (at `ε = 1e-3` the spectrum sits on the imaginary axis — a fundamental Bromwich-inversion limit, not a tuning defect; a shippable hyperbolic variant requires construction-time sector fitting `α < π/2 − β` per Weideman–Trefethen 2007 and possibly rational-Krylov; see ADR-0148 for the full TRIZ analysis and Hale–Weideman 2015 §5 for the ND extension feasibility).

**Mathematical claim (NORMATIVE).** For a self-adjoint sectorial generator `A` on a 2D or 3D tensor-product domain (divergence-form Laplacian via Kronecker sum, Neumann BC, row-major storage matching `grid2d.rs` / `grid3d.rs`), the TWS parabolic-contour quadrature

```text
e^{tA} g ≈ (1/2πi) Σ_k e^{λ_k t} (λ_k I − A)⁻¹ g · λ'(θ_k) · (2π/M)     (47.8)
```

with the **same** `(a_0, a_1, a_2) = (0.1309, 0.1194, 0.2500)` parabolic optimum (§47.2) and `M/t` cost-decoupling scaling converges **geometrically** in `M` at the same rate as the 1D case. The outer quadrature is **dimension-blind** (Hale–Weideman 2015 Theorem 3.1): the convergence rate depends only on the contour geometry and the sectorial sector half-angle of `A`, not on the spatial dimension. The ONLY new primitive is the per-node linear solve `(λ_k I − A)⁻¹ g`: the 1D complex Thomas is replaced by a **banded complex direct solve** (half-bandwidth `bw = nx` in 2D, `bw = nx·ny` in 3D) via Gaussian elimination — `O(N·bw²)` unconditionally stable off-spectrum for sectorial `A` (since `λ_k ∉ σ(A)` by contour construction).

**Kronecker-sum structure.** For 2D (row-major `idx(i,j) = j·nx + i`): `A = I_y ⊗ L_x + L_y ⊗ I_x`, so `(λI − A)` has the bandwidth-`nx` banded structure. For 3D (`idx(i,j,k) = k·nx·ny + j·nx + i`): `A = I_z ⊗ I_y ⊗ L_x + I_z ⊗ L_y ⊗ I_x + L_z ⊗ I_y ⊗ I_x`, bandwidth `nx·ny`. The Neumann diagonal rows use `1/dx²` (one-sided), interior rows `2/dx²` (both sides) — mirroring the 1D Thomas stencil entry-for-entry.

**NARROW restriction (§47.4 extended).** Self-adjoint negative-semidefinite generators only — every shipped 2D/3D divergence-form kernel (`Strang2D<DiffusionChernoff,…>`, `Strang3D<…>`, etc.). Non-self-adjoint / advection-dominated 2D/3D generators are OUT of scope for v8.2.0 for the same reason as 1D: Theorem 47.1 requires a sectorial spectrum, and no shipped 2D/3D kernel violates this. The **hyperbolic contour** for non-sectorial 2D/3D operators remains deferred (ADR-0148 — cite Weideman–Trefethen 2007 for optimal `(μ,α,h)` fitting and Hale–Weideman 2015 for the ND extension precedent).

**Acceptance gates (NORMATIVE):**
- `G_RESOLVENT_JUMP_2D_ORDER` (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`): OLS slope `d log‖e_M‖_∞ / d log(1/M) ≥ +1.95` at `t = 100`, `M ∈ {6,8,10,12,14}`, `16×16` 2D Neumann Laplacian. Self-convergence reference `M_ref = 40`. Measured (Rust gate): `+9.81`. Matches pre-flight oracle `+9.97` (Python `scripts/resolvent_jump_2d3d_kit.py` A3).
- `G_RESOLVENT_JUMP_3D_ORDER` (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`): same spec, `N = 8³`. Measured: `+9.75`. Pre-flight `+9.79` (kit A5).
- `T_RESOLVENT_JUMP_ND` (NORMATIVE oracle, `scripts/resolvent_jump_2d3d_kit.py`): 5/5 PART A sub-checks PASS. Integrated into `xtask test-fast` sympy sweep; prints `T_RESOLVENT_JUMP_ND PASS` on success.

**Sign convention (G24 — SAME as §47.5 / G_RESOLVENT_JUMP_ORDER):** positive slope = convergence as `M` grows (`xs = 1/M`; `≥ +1.95` PASSES). Do NOT re-derive; copy §47.5 verbatim.

**Implementation note.** `resolvent_jump_nd.rs` (sibling to `resolvent_jump.rs`) reuses `contour_node` (`pub(crate)`) unchanged. Each new type (`ResolventJumpChernoff2D<F>`, `ResolventJumpChernoff3D<F>`) holds only `(grid, m_nodes)` — no additional state. The banded Gaussian elimination is implemented inline without external dependencies (`no_std + alloc`), consistent with the project's zero-dep constraint.

## §48 — Eigenbasis-rotation separability for off-diagonal anisotropic diffusion — `EigenrotatedAnisotropicChernoff` (EXPLORED — DEFERRED, NOT SHIPPED in v8.0.0; ADR-0137 DEMOTED; CONTINUOUS-OPERATOR mathematics retained)

> **§48 STATUS — DEFERRED, NOT SHIPPED (2026-06-07, review finding C2).** The F5 kernel
> `EigenrotatedAnisotropicChernoff` was **withdrawn** from the v8.0.0 ship. The shipped
> implementation did NOT deliver the `D·q` node reduction that is the entire premise of §48:
> it looped the full `q^D` tensor quadrature and back-rotated each node point-wise through
> `Q`, then sampled via the `2^D`-corner multilinear interpolant — **more expensive than the
> §32 sibling**, for zero correctness gain (§32 already handles off-diagonal `A` correctly via
> Cholesky). The genuine `D·q` algorithm is **blocked on a tensor grid**: §48.3's `R_{Qᵀ}`
> resample lands eigen-coordinates `y=Qᵀx` between grid points, so a grid-wide `O(N·2^D)`
> multilinear resample is required to reach the separable per-axis sweep — and that resample
> is **not an isometry**, injecting an `O(dx²)` per-step interpolation floor that BREAKS the
> Theorem 48.1 "zero rotation error" exactness (which is a *continuous-operator* identity the
> discrete grid cannot honor). The `D·q` node-count win survives only at this new accuracy
> cost — a real-but-bounded speedup, NOT the exact, free, 125× win specced here.
>
> **What §48 remains good for:** the *continuous-operator* spectral identity
> `e^{τA}=Qe^{τΛ}Qᵀ` (§48.2-§48.4, certified by the `T_EIGENBASIS` sympy oracle) is TRUE and
> is retained as the math foundation for any future genuine D·q kernel. The NORMATIVE-library
> claims below (eq. 48.4 as a shipped discrete kernel, the `D·q` node-count win, the
> RELEASE_BLOCKING gate) are **SUPERSEDED / WITHDRAWN** — read §48.2-§48.4 as continuous
> theory, not as a shipped algorithm. See ADR-0137 "Demotion analysis" for the full ruling.


### §48.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

For a **constant** symmetric-positive-definite (SPD) diffusion tensor `A ∈ ℝ^{D×D}` with nonzero off-diagonal entries (`a_{ij} ≠ 0`, `i ≠ j`), the divergence-form generator
$$
L \;=\; \nabla\!\cdot(A\nabla) \;=\; \sum_{i,j=1}^{D} A_{ij}\,\partial^2_{x_i x_j} \tag{48.1}
$$
is **non-separable in the standard coordinate axes**: its Fourier symbol `−ξᵀAξ` carries cross terms `−A_{ij}ξ_iξ_j`. The shipped `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND<F,D>` (§32, ADR-0081) handles this *correctly* — its Cholesky factor `A = LLᵀ` shifts the Gauss-Hermite stencil along the correlated directions — but it still draws nodes from the **full tensor-product** quadrature lattice `η ∈ {GH₅}^D`, costing `q^D` quadrature points per grid point (`q = 5`; `5^5 = 3125` at `D = 5`). The cross terms force the lattice to remain `D`-dimensional even after the §44 Smolyak sparsification (ADR-0123), because Smolyak exploits sparsity in a **fixed** coordinate frame, not the principal-axis frame.

This section rotates the problem into the eigenbasis of `A`, where the operator becomes **axis-aligned by construction**, so the existing **per-axis** anisotropic 1D kernel (Strang/Lie product of `D` independent 1D Gauss-Hermite shifts) applies with `D·q` nodes instead of `q^D`. This is **distinct** from Smolyak (sparse tensor in a fixed frame, §44) and from the ζ² post-quadrature correction (applied *after* quadrature in the original frame, §32.8, ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 2).

### §48.2 — Spectral decomposition and the rotated operator (CITATION — Horn & Johnson 2013 Thm 4.1.5)

Since `A` is symmetric SPD, the spectral theorem gives an **orthogonal** `Q ∈ O(D)` (`QᵀQ = QQᵀ = I`) and a diagonal `Λ = diag(λ_1, …, λ_D)` with `λ_i > 0` such that
$$
A \;=\; Q\,\Lambda\,Q^{\!\top}, \qquad Q^{\!\top}\!A\,Q \;=\; \Lambda. \tag{48.2}
$$
Introduce the **constant linear change of variables** `y = Qᵀx` (`x = Q y`). Because `Q` is constant, `∂_{x} = Q\,∂_{y}` (chain rule with constant Jacobian `Qᵀ`), and the second-order part transforms as
$$
\sum_{i,j} A_{ij}\,\partial^2_{x_i x_j}
\;=\; \partial_x^{\!\top} A\,\partial_x
\;=\; \partial_y^{\!\top}\,(Q^{\!\top}\!A\,Q)\,\partial_y
\;=\; \partial_y^{\!\top} \Lambda\,\partial_y
\;=\; \sum_{i=1}^{D} \lambda_i\,\partial^2_{y_i y_i}. \tag{48.3}
$$
The rotated operator `L̃ = Σ_i λ_i ∂²_{y_i y_i}` is **diagonal / separable**: its symbol `−ηᵀΛη = −Σ_i λ_iη_i²` (with `η = Qᵀξ`) contains **no cross term** `η_iη_j`, `i ≠ j`. The single-axis pieces `λ_i ∂²_{y_i}` mutually commute, so the semigroup factorizes exactly: `e^{τL̃} = ∏_i e^{τλ_i ∂²_{y_i}}` (no Strang BCH residue — pairwise commutation, identical to the §10.6 / Lemma 10.1 tensor-product collapse).

### §48.3 — The eigenbasis-rotation Chernoff step (NORMATIVE library)

For a state `f` sampled on the standard-axis grid, one time step of the F5 kernel is the **rotate-in → diagonal-step → rotate-out** sandwich:
$$
F_{\mathrm{eig}}(\tau)\,f
\;=\;
R_{Q^{\!\top}}^{-1}\,\Bigl[\,\textstyle\prod_{i=1}^{D} S_i(\lambda_i, \tau)\,\Bigr]\,R_{Q^{\!\top}}\,f,
\qquad
(R_{Q^{\!\top}} g)(y) := g(Q y), \tag{48.4}
$$
where `R_{Qᵀ}` resamples the grid function into eigen-coordinates `y = Qᵀx`, each `S_i(λ_i, τ)` is the **existing per-axis 1D anisotropic Gauss-Hermite shift** along eigen-axis `i` with scalar diffusion `λ_i` (the 1D specialization of §32.4 eq. 32.3, `D·q` nodes total across the `D` axes), and `R_{Qᵀ}^{-1} = R_Q` rotates back. Drift `b` and reaction `c`, when present and constant, rotate identically (`b ↦ Qᵀb`, `c` invariant).
>
> **DISCRETE OBSTRUCTION (WITHDRAWN-ship caveat).** The `D·q`-nodes property of eq. 48.4 holds ONLY if `[∏_i S_i]` acts as `D` separable 1D convolutions — which requires `f` sampled on an **eigen-aligned** tensor grid. `R_{Qᵀ}` is exact as an *operator* but on a standard-axis grid it is a `D`-dimensional resample (`y=Qᵀx` falls between grid points), `O(N·2^D)` multilinear and **non-isometric** (`O(dx²)` per-step floor). A naive discrete realization that keeps the standard grid and back-rotates each tensor node (the path the withdrawn F5 code took) does NOT separate — it stays `q^D`. Hence eq. 48.4 is a continuous identity, deferred as a shipped algorithm (see §48 STATUS banner).

### §48.4 — Exactness and order-of-accuracy (NORMATIVE library — the central claim)

> **Theorem 48.1 (rotation-exactness, constant `A`).** Let `A` be constant SPD with spectral decomposition (48.2). Let `S(τ)` be any Chernoff function for the scalar/per-axis diffusion family with global order `p` (`‖S(τ/n)^n f − e^{τL̃}f‖ = O(n^{−p})` on its core). Then the eigenbasis-rotation kernel (48.4) satisfies
> $$
> \bigl\| F_{\mathrm{eig}}(\tau/n)^n f \;-\; e^{\tau L} f \bigr\| \;=\; O(n^{-p}),
> $$
> i.e. it **inherits the order `p` of the inner per-axis kernel with ZERO additional rotation error.**

*Proof sketch (NORMATIVE).* `Q` is a **constant orthogonal** operator, hence `R_{Qᵀ}` is a bounded invertible isometry that **commutes with the time variable** (it acts on space only and does not depend on `τ` or `n`). By the spectral mapping theorem, for any analytic `h`, `h(L) = R_{Qᵀ}^{-1} h(L̃) R_{Qᵀ}` exactly — in particular for `h = e^{τ(·)}` the heat semigroups satisfy `e^{τL} = R_{Qᵀ}^{-1} e^{τL̃} R_{Qᵀ}` with **no error**. Therefore
$$
F_{\mathrm{eig}}(\tau/n)^n
= R_{Qᵀ}^{-1}\,\bigl[\textstyle\prod_i S_i(\lambda_i,\tau/n)\bigr]^n\,R_{Qᵀ}
$$
and the entire approximation error is carried by the inner product `[∏_i S_i]^n`, which converges to `e^{τL̃}` at the inner order `p`. The isometry `R_{Qᵀ}` is removed exactly on both sides. ∎

This is certified symbolically by the **T_EIGENBASIS** oracle (`scripts/eigenbasis_rotation_kit.py`, §48.6): for representative off-diagonal SPD tensors at `D = 3` and `D = 5` it verifies (i) `QᵀAQ = Λ` diagonal with `QᵀQ = I` and `λ_i > 0`; (ii) the rotated symbol `−ηᵀΛη` has no cross term and equals `−ξᵀAξ` under `η = Qᵀξ`; (iii) the **exact** matrix identity `e^{τA} = Q e^{τΛ} Qᵀ` (`τ` symbolic) — the order-preservation / rotation-exactness certificate. PRE-FLIGHT RESULT 2026-06-07: **T_EIGENBASIS PASS** (both dimensions, Pyright-clean, exit 0).

**Node-count win (WITHDRAWN — see §48 STATUS banner).** ~~The standard-frame tensor kernel uses `q^D` quadrature nodes per grid point; the eigenbasis per-axis kernel uses `D·q`. At `q = 5`: `D = 5 ⇒ 3125 → 25` (125×), `D = 6 ⇒ 15625 → 30` (520×).~~ **FALSE for the shipped kernel and unattainable as specced.** The shipped F5 code looped `q^D` quadrature nodes (NO `D·q` reduction) and back-rotated each point-wise through `Q`, plus a `2^D`-corner resample per node — strictly *more* expensive than the §32 `q^D` baseline. The genuine `D·q` algorithm would require rotating the WHOLE grid into an eigen-aligned grid ONCE (an `O(N·2^D)` multilinear resample, repeated for rotate-out), doing `D` sequential 1D GH5 convolutions there (`D·q` quadrature taps), then rotating back. That recovers the `D·q` **quadrature** node count, but the discrete resample is *not* an isometry and injects an `O(dx²)` per-step interpolation floor — so the eq. 48.4 "zero rotation error" exactness (a continuous-operator property) does NOT survive on the grid. Net: a real `O(N·(D·q + 2·2^D))` cost vs. `O(N·q^D)`, but with a NEW accuracy penalty that §32 (no resample) does not pay. DEFERRED — not shipped in v8.0.0.

### §48.5 — Honest scope: constant (or piecewise-constant) `A` ONLY (NORMATIVE library)

The rotation-exactness of Theorem 48.1 hinges on `Q` being a **constant** orthogonal map that commutes with the time-stepping. **This holds if and only if `A` is constant** (or piecewise-constant on subdomains, with the rotation applied per piece). For a **spatially-varying** tensor `A(x)`, the diagonalizing rotation `Q(x)` is itself `x`-dependent, so `R_{Q(x)ᵀ}` no longer commutes with `∂`: the change of variables introduces a **first-order commutator residual** `[Q(x), ∂]` (concretely, gradient-of-`Q` terms `∂_x Q(x)` that contaminate the rotated operator with non-diagonal lower-order parts). The eigenbasis kernel is therefore **NOT order-exact for variable `A(x)`** — it would carry an `O(τ)` per-step rotation error analogous to (but distinct from) the §32 frozen-coefficient mismatch. This **variable-`A(x)` eigenbasis residual** is explicitly **DEFERRED** (named here for traceability; out of scope for v8.0.0). Users with genuinely spatially-varying off-diagonal `A(x)` MUST use the shipped `AnisotropicShiftChernoffND<F,D>` (§32, Cholesky-in-the-original-frame, correct at the `q^D` cost) or its ζ² order-2 lift (§32.8). The F5 kernel is a **constant-`A` cost optimization**, not a new accuracy class.

### §48.6 — Acceptance gate G_EIGENBASIS_ANISO_DDIM (ADVISORY) + T_EIGENBASIS (NORMATIVE)

- **`G_EIGENBASIS_ANISO_DDIM`** (ADVISORY — does NOT block release; ADR-0137, `slow-tests`): off-diagonal anisotropic self-convergence at `D ≥ 5`. Build `EigenrotatedAnisotropicChernoff<_, f64, 5>` for a constant off-diagonal SPD tensor `A` (anisotropy ratio `λ_max/λ_min ≳ 8`), Gaussian datum, `T = 0.5`. Sweep `n ∈ {16, 32, 64, 128}`; reference is the finest companion step. The `log`-`log` OLS self-convergence slope MUST be `≤ −1.95` (order-2 inner per-axis kernel inherited per Theorem 48.1). **ADVISORY rationale:** the *correctness* of F5 (exactness for constant `A`) is fully certified by the **symbolic** T_EIGENBASIS oracle, which is deterministic and frame-independent; the convergence-slope gate is a numerical *regression sentinel* for the per-axis interpolation floor (the same coarse-grid `O(n·dx²)` floor that forced the §32.5 G_DDIM AMENDMENT 1 ladder). Because ADR-0137 proposed **no** gate and the headline accuracy claim rests on the symbolic oracle (not the slope), the slope gate is advisory: a floor-dominated flattening should **warn**, not block a MINOR cost-optimization release. It MAY be promoted to RELEASE_BLOCKING in a later PATCH once the coarse-grid ladder is calibrated for the eigen-rotated stencil (mirrors the L-gate advisory→blocking promotion mechanic of §3.6.bis.7).

- **`T_EIGENBASIS`** (NORMATIVE numeric+symbolic oracle — ADR-0137, `scripts/eigenbasis_rotation_kit.py`): the three sub-checks of §48.4 at `D ∈ {3, 5}`. Prints exactly `T_EIGENBASIS PASS` / `T_EIGENBASIS FAIL: <reason>`. Pure symbolic — **no library runtime** — so it runs in the `test-fast` sympy sweep without `slow-tests`. Failure **BLOCKS** v8.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity precedent (the symbolic exactness IS the F5 correctness contract).

### §48.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Constant / piecewise-constant `A` only** (§48.5). Variable `A(x)` eigenbasis residual `[Q(x), ∂]` deferred (named, out of scope v8.0.0).
- **Symmetric SPD `A` required.** The orthogonal diagonalization (48.2) needs `A = Aᵀ` (true for every diffusion tensor in this library). Non-symmetric / non-normal generators have no real orthogonal eigenbasis and are out of scope.
- **Real, distinct-or-repeated spectrum.** Repeated eigenvalues are fine (any orthonormal basis of the eigenspace works); the construction picks a canonical one. Complex spectra do not arise for symmetric `A`.
- **Inner kernel choice.** v8.0.0 specifies the per-axis 1D anisotropic Gauss-Hermite shift (`S_i`) as the inner kernel (order-2 with the §32.8 ζ² correction available per-axis). A higher-order inner per-axis kernel (e.g. the §27 ζ⁴ family) would lift the whole F5 kernel to that order with the SAME zero-rotation-error guarantee (Theorem 48.1 is inner-kernel-agnostic) — deferred.

### §48.8 — References

- R. A. Horn, C. R. Johnson, *Matrix Analysis*, 2nd ed., Cambridge Univ. Press (2013), Theorem 4.1.5 (spectral theorem for real symmetric matrices: orthogonal diagonalization `A = QΛQᵀ`).
- G. H. Golub, C. F. Van Loan, *Matrix Computations*, 4th ed., Johns Hopkins (2013), §8.5 (symmetric eigenproblem; cyclic Jacobi rotation for small dense symmetric matrices).
- I. D. Remizov, *Chernoff approximation of operator semigroups …*, **Vladikavkaz Math. J.** 27:4 (2025), Theorem 3 cousin (the per-axis anisotropic shift kernel `S_i` reused here, via §32 / ADR-0081).
- math §32 / ADR-0081 (`AnisotropicShiftChernoffND` — the Cholesky-in-original-frame baseline F5 optimizes); §32.8 / ADR-0112 AMENDMENT 2 (ζ² order-2 correction — composable per-axis); §44 / ADR-0123 (Smolyak — DISTINCT: sparse tensor in a fixed frame, not the principal-axis frame); §10.6 / Lemma 10.1 (commuting per-axis tensor-product semigroup collapse — the zero-BCH-residue precedent reused in §48.2).
- ADR-0137 (F5 eigenbasis-rotation separability — PROPOSED → ACCEPTED at this spike).
