## §49 — Dynamic Wentzell/Robin Boundary Conditions via Implicit Cayley Boundary Step (NORMATIVE)

**Kernel:** `DynamicWentzellChernoff<C, R, F>` (module `wentzell.rs`, ADR-0151, v8.2.0 Wave-2 C-9).

**Status:** NORMATIVE. Implementation: `crates/semiflow-core/src/wentzell.rs`. Gates: `G_WENTZELL_STABLE` (RELEASE_BLOCKING), `G_WENTZELL_ORDER` (RELEASE_BLOCKING), `T_WENTZELL` (NORMATIVE oracle, `scripts/wentzell_robin_stability_preflight.py`).

### §49.1 — Problem setting: dynamic Wentzell/Robin BC

Consider the heat equation on `[0, ∞)` with a dynamic boundary condition at `x = 0`:

```
∂_t u = a(x) ∂_xx u            (bulk, x > 0)
∂_t u + γ(t) ∂_ν u + c·u = 0  (boundary ODE at x = 0, outward normal ∂_ν = −∂_x)
```

where `γ(t) ≥ 0` is a time-dependent scaling and `c ≥ 0` is a boundary reaction coefficient.

The reformulation as a coupled PDAE on `X ⊕ ℝ_∂` (1D: `X ⊕ L²(∂Ω)` collapses to `X ⊕ ℝ`) gives a semigroup generator with **unbounded** off-diagonal coupling `−γ(t)/dx` (the discrete normal-derivative `∂_ν`). Stephan 2023 (arXiv:2307.00419, ZAMM 2025) proves the **explicit** (forward-Euler/Trotter) product formula diverges: `‖T(t/n)^n‖ ≥ n^β → ∞` (§5, relative-bound exponent `β ∈ (0,1]`). This obstruction is explicit-only (ADR-0146 Conclusion).

### §49.2 — Lie splitting: bulk + implicit Cayley boundary sub-step

Per step `[t, t + τ]`, `DynamicWentzellChernoff.apply_at(t, τ, …)` performs a **bulk–boundary Lie split** (Altmann–Verfürth 2021, arXiv:2108.08147):

1. **Bulk Chernoff step (factor (a)):** `dst = C(τ) src` via `self.inner.apply_into(τ, src, dst, scratch)` (the inner `DiffusionChernoff<f64>` step; any bulk Chernoff function that implements `ChernoffFunction<f64, S = GridFn1D<f64>>` is admissible).

2. **Implicit Cayley boundary sub-step (factor (b)):** Advance `[dst[1], dst[0]]` (first interior node + boundary trace DOF) by the `2×2`-per-boundary-DOF Cayley map.

The time-dependent `γ(t)` is frozen at the left endpoint `t_k` (Howland §23 freeze): `γ_k = γ(t_k)`. The per-step Cayley amplification with the frozen-γ block has `ρ ≤ 1` unconditionally (ADR-0146 stability verdict: GO; §49.5 gate).

### §49.3 — The 2×2 boundary generator block `C_∂`

At the near-boundary DOF pair `[u_bulk, u_∂]` (bulk interior node `u[1]` + boundary trace `u[0]`), the generator of the coupled system (with `γ` frozen at step start) is:

```
C_∂(γ, c, a₀, dx) = [[ −a₀/dx²          +1/dx         ]
                      [ −γ/dx          −(γ/dx + c)     ]]
```

Row 0 = near-boundary interior mode (diffusion eigenvalue `−a₀·κ²` at `κ = π/dx`; weak boundary feedback `+1/dx`).
Row 1 = boundary trace DOF (stiff coupling `−γ/dx`; dissipative reaction `−(γ/dx + c)`).

The `(1,0)` entry `−γ/dx = O(1/dx) → ∞` is the **unbounded coupling** that Stephan's §5 makes the explicit product diverge. The eigenvalues of `C_∂` lie in the **closed left half-plane** (dissipative, verified by the `diag(1, dx)` weighted inner product; ADR-0146 §Stability).

### §49.4 — Cayley map: closed-form 2×2 Crank–Nicolson

The implicit Cayley (Crank–Nicolson) step on the `2×2` block is:

```
K_CN = (I − (τ/2)·C_∂)⁻¹ (I + (τ/2)·C_∂)
```

The `2×2` inverse is computed in closed form via the adjugate:

```
(I − (τ/2)·C_∂)⁻¹ = adj(I − (τ/2)·C_∂) / det(I − (τ/2)·C_∂)
```

No LAPACK; no_std-safe. The determinant is `det = (1 + (τ/2)(a₀/dx² + γ/dx + c))(1 + (τ/2)(a₀/dx²)) − (τ/2)²(γ/dx)(1/dx)` (positive for `a₀, γ, c, τ, dx > 0`; see §49.5 stability proof).

The SYMBOLIC witness (sympy, `τ, μ > 0`): the Cayley symbol at eigenvalue `λ = −μ` is `z_cay(μ) = (1 − τμ/2)/(1 + τμ/2)`, and `1 − z_cay² = 8μτ/(μ²τ² + 4μτ + 4) ≥ 0` for all `μ, τ > 0`, so `|z_cay| ≤ 1` unconditionally. The stiff limit is `lim_{μ→∞} z_cay = −1` (marginal; never exceeds 1). The explicit symbol `z_expl = 1 − τμ → −∞` (UNSTABLE).

### §49.5 — Gate G_WENTZELL_STABLE (RELEASE_BLOCKING)

**File:** `crates/semiflow-core/tests/g_wentzell_stable.rs`. Feature: `slow-tests`. Function: `g_wentzell_stable` (`#[ignore]`).

**Sweep:** `dx ∈ {1/16, 1/64, 1/256, 1/1024}`, `γ ∈ {0.5, 1, 4, 16}`, `κ = π/dx`, `τ = 0.4·dx²/a`.

**Assertions:**
1. `ρ(K_CN) ≤ 1 + 1e-9` for every `(dx, γ)` pair (A-stable, unconditional).
2. `ρ(I + τ·C_∂) > 1` for at least one `(dx, γ)` pair (the explicit map IS unstable — the Cayley step fixes a real instability, not a trivially-stable regime).

**Pre-flight result (ADR-0146):** Cayley max `ρ = 0.999804 ≤ 1`; explicit max `ρ = 2.9478 > 1`. ✓

### §49.6 — Gate G_WENTZELL_ORDER (RELEASE_BLOCKING)

**File:** `crates/semiflow-core/tests/g_wentzell_order.rs`. Feature: `slow-tests`. Function: `g_wentzell_order` (`#[ignore]`).

**Method:** Self-convergence (no closed-form oracle for dynamic Wentzell BCs). Reference = N_REF = 512 Chernoff steps. Sweep `n ∈ {16, 32, 64, 128}`. Spatial probe at `x = 0.35 · DOMAIN_MAX` (non-origin, non-midpoint — symmetric-cancellation avoidance per the G24 lesson).

**Initial datum:** `u₀(x) = sin²(πx/L) · e^{−x/2}` (smooth, zero at `x = 0` — compatible with Wentzell BC start condition; non-zero in interior).

**Time-dependent `γ`:** `γ(t) = 0.5 + sin(t)` (generic; never identically static or zero).

**Gate:** OLS slope `d log‖err‖_∞ / d log(τ) ≤ −0.95` (order-1, consistent with Altmann–Verfürth Lie splitting first-order theorem and static Robin precedent ADR-0098).

**Weak CFL note:** A weak CFL `τ ≤ c·h` is an ACCURACY requirement for the Lie splitting commutator error (not a stability collapse — stability is unconditional by the Cayley bound).

### §49.7 — Deferred: multi-D product state and second-order BDF variant

The 1D construction collapses `X ⊕ L²(∂Ω) → X ⊕ ℝ_∂` (the boundary trace DOF is `dst.values[0]`). Multi-D requires a true `X ⊕ L²(∂Ω)` product state with a separate `GridFn1D` or `GridFn2D` boundary function — **deferred to v8.x** (different `type S`; requires new State impl).

A second-order BDF / Strang boundary variant (Altmann–Verfürth 2022, arXiv:2209.07835) that achieves slope `≤ −1.95` is also **deferred** (requires a two-step boundary solve, non-trivial state history).

Per-cell-varying `γ(x, t)` along `∂Ω` (anisotropic Wentzell BC) is **deferred to v8.x**.

### §49.8 — Order analysis

`DynamicWentzellChernoff::order() = 1`. The commutator `[C(τ), K_CN(τ)]` between the bulk Chernoff operator `C(τ)` (acting on interior DOFs) and the boundary Cayley step `K_CN(τ)` (acting on `[u[1], u[0]]`) is nonzero: the bulk step samples `u[1]` before the boundary step modifies `u[0]`, and the Lie splitting residual is `O(τ²)` per step → `O(τ)` globally (first-order). Additionally, the left-endpoint freeze `γ(t_k)` of the time-dependent coefficient contributes an `O(τ)` per-step splitting error. Both sources are consistent with order 1. This matches the static Robin precedent (ADR-0098, math §3.5.tris.5) and the Altmann–Verfürth Lie splitting theorem (first-order in `τ` under a weak CFL `τ ≤ ch`).

### §49.9 — References

- R. Altmann, C. Verfürth, *Bulk-surface Lie splitting for parabolic problems with dynamic boundary conditions*, arXiv:2108.08147; *IMA J. Numer. Anal.* (2023). — implicit-Euler sub-step splitting, unconditional sub-step stability, weak CFL `τ ≤ ch`, first-order convergence.
- R. Altmann, C. Verfürth, *A second-order bulk–surface splitting…*, arXiv:2209.07835; *IMA J. Numer. Anal.* (2023). — second-order BDF decoupling (deferred §49.7).
- B. Kovács, C. Lubich, *Numerical analysis of parabolic problems with dynamic boundary conditions*, arXiv:1501.01882; *IMA J. Numer. Anal.* 37:1 (2017). — A-stable implicit integrators (backward Euler, BDF, Radau IIA) stable for dynamic Wentzell BC on `L²(Ω) ⊕ L²(∂Ω)`.
- A. Stephan, *Trotter-type formula for operator semigroups on product spaces*, arXiv:2307.00419; ZAMM 105:9 (2025). — explicit freezing product diverges for unbounded coupling (§5); the obstruction is explicit-only (ADR-0146 conclusion).
- A. Iserles, *A First Course in the Numerical Analysis of Differential Equations* (Cambridge 2009), §8 — Cayley/Möbius map A-stability (the §17.4 precedent reused at the boundary block level).
- ADR-0151 (engineer spec), ADR-0146 (stability research + TRIZ GO verdict), ADR-0098 (static Robin sibling), math §17.4 (Crank–Nicolson Cayley map — §17.4 precedent), math §23 (Howland nonautonomous lift — `γ(t)` vehicle).

---

## §50 — Gridless transition-law Chernoff evolver on a particle ensemble — `GridlessChernoff` (v9.0.0 SHIP-NARROW, ADR-0155, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics — third S-curve, R1)

> **§50 STATUS — SHIP-NARROW (d=2 validated particle primitive + NEGATIVE RESULT, v9.0.0).** This
> section specifies the particle GridlessChernoff and documents the full honest arc of the high-d
> investigation. The sympy oracle **`T_GRIDLESS_*` is PASS** (`scripts/gridless_kit.py` 3/3
> sub-checks: push_forward_exactness / mass_conservation / voronoi_moment_match; commit `f633cde`).
> The Rust gates were **MEASURED** under a fair shared-CRN protocol (ADR-0155 Amendment, 2026-06-09):
> `G_GRIDLESS_DIM_SCALING` — **d=2 PASS** (err 1.197e-3 < 5e-3); d=3 needs 8× cap; d≥4 accuracy
> collapses (err 9.75e-2 … 7.05e-1) — **INTRINSIC LIMIT** (§50.7: spatial-merge curse re-enters
> reduction grid). `G_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE` — **NO-GO**: deterministic branching beats MC only 1.417×
> (MSE ratio) at d=2, below the pre-registered ≥2× gate (§50.6); low-variance thesis not confirmed.
> **The root cause** (documented as INTRINSIC LIMIT, §50.7): the Chernoff branching is a deterministic
> quadrature; its error is bias; reducing bias in `d` dimensions in a **particle** representation
> requires `O(m^d)` bins — the curse of dimensionality re-enters through the reduction grid. The
> variance thesis was not confirmed even at d=2.
>
> **THE CURSE IS AN ARTIFACT OF THE PARTICLE CARRIER, NOT OF THE EVOLVER.** The resolution is the
> **tensor-train carrier** documented in **§52** (ADR-0159): holding the state as a low-rank TT
> with the separable per-axis Chernoff shift as a rank-preserving (O(1)-mode, solver-free) operator
> escapes the exponential curse for the linear diagonal-A (Gaussian) class — deterministically,
> `no_std`, byte-reproducibly. See §52 for the shipped `TtChernoff` and its gate
> `G_TT_CHERNOFF_DIMSCALING`. **This section (§50) is the honest record of the particle form** —
> d=2 validated deterministic primitive (retained as a correct library component) and the negative
> result (four reframes all refuted under the particle representation; see §50.7). The particle form
> does NOT escape the high-d curse; §52 does.
>
> **v9.0.0 headline**: Shift B (`ReverseChernoff`, §51) is the co-headline. Shift C ships as:
> (a) `GridlessChernoff` d=2 narrow particle primitive + negative result (§50), AND
> (b) `TtChernoff` TT-carrier curse-escape for the diagonal-A Gaussian class (§52).

### §50.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

A Cartesian `GridND<F,D>` costs `O(N^d)` time and memory; `SmolyakGridND` (§44, ADR-0123) reaches `D=6` before blow-up. The **third S-curve resource R1** is that Theorem-6 formula (6)
$$
S(\tau)f(x) = \tfrac14 f(x{+}2\sqrt{a\tau}) + \tfrac14 f(x{-}2\sqrt{a\tau}) + \tfrac12 f(x{+}2b\tau) + \tau c\,f(x) \tag{50.1}
$$
*is a Markov transition kernel*: the weights `¼,¼,½` on the three deterministic shifts are a (sub-)probability branching law, and the §38 adjoint `S*(τ)` pushes a **measure** forward exactly as these shifts. Iterating (50.1) on a measure/particle ensemble `ρ = Σᵢ wᵢ δ_{xᵢ}` rather than a grid makes one Chernoff step *one branching push-forward step* at `O(d·P)` cost (`P` = particle count) **independent of an ambient grid resolution `N`**. The shipped `AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff<C,F,D>` + `MeasureState<F,D>` (§38.9, v8.0.0) is this evolver *in embryo*; this section turns its gate-only Dirac-fold trick into a general bounded-`d` evolver.

### §50.2 — The particle/measure state and the one-step push-forward (NORMATIVE library)

The state is a finite signed measure on `ℝ^d` represented as a weighted particle ensemble
$$
\rho \;=\; \sum_{i=1}^{P} w_i\,\delta_{x_i}, \qquad x_i \in \mathbb{R}^d,\; w_i \in \mathbb{R}, \tag{50.2}
$$
optionally augmented by a Gaussian-smoothed background (§50.4). One step of the evolver is the **§38 adjoint kernel** `S*(τ)` applied particlewise. By Lemma A.1 (§38.3), with push-forward `(τ_a ρ)(B) := ρ(B − a)`,
$$
S^*(\tau)\,\delta_{x}
\;=\; \tfrac14\,\delta_{x + h(x)} + \tfrac14\,\delta_{x - h(x)} + \tfrac12\,\delta_{x + k(x)} + \tau c(x)\,\delta_{x}, \tag{50.3}
$$
with anisotropic step vectors `h(x) = 2\sqrt{a(x)\tau}` (per-axis, Cholesky-correlated for off-diagonal `A`, §32.4) and `k(x) = 2 b(x)\tau`. Applied to (50.2) by linearity, one step maps `P` particles to (at most) `3P` particles with reweighting `w_i ↦ w_i·(1 + \tau c(x_i))`. **Sign convention (NORMATIVE, mirrors §38.3):** the `+h`/`−h` diffusion branches are symmetric about `x`; the drift branch is `+k = +2b\tau` (forward drift) on the **adjoint/measure** side — note this is the *push-forward* direction, opposite in sign to the backward `f`-evolver of (50.1) under the §38.2 dual pairing `⟨S(τ)f, ρ⟩ = ⟨f, S*(τ)ρ⟩`. The reaction `τc` multiplies mass, not position.

> *NORMATIVE (d-dim realization).* For diagonal A the step (50.3) is applied **per-axis on
> every one of the `d` axes** as a sequential splitting sweep (commuting axes ⇒ exact
> splitting; reaction applied once globally as `(1+τc)`). An implementation that perturbs only
> one axis for `D>1` does NOT realize `e^{τL}` and is non-conformant. The step vector
> `h(x)=2√(a(x)τ)` of eq. 50.3 is **per-axis** `h_j = 2√(a_j τ)` — one component per axis,
> not a single scalar applied to axis 0.

### §50.3 — The `4ⁿ` obstruction (NORMATIVE library — the central difficulty)

Iterating (50.3) `n` times grows the Dirac count as `3ⁿ`–`4ⁿ` (each particle branches into 3 new positions per step; with a retained `x` reaction-Dirac, ≤4). This is **worse than the grid it escapes** unless reduced. §38.9 records that the v8.0.0 gate sidesteps this only for the *Brownian self-convergence test* via a closed-form characteristic-function Dirac-fold `⟨\cos(ξx), Σwᵢδ_{xᵢ}⟩ = Σwᵢ\cos(ξx_i)` (`O(n_diracs)` cost), which does **not** generalize to a working evolver for arbitrary data/functionals. The general fix is a **particle-reduction operator** (§50.4) applied each (or every `m`) step to cap `P`.

### §50.4 — Particle-reduction operator and its error (NORMATIVE library)

Define a reduction map `R_P : M(ℝ^d) → M_P(ℝ^d)` projecting onto at most `P` particles. Two concrete forms (ship-track uses the first; the second is the long-time fallback recorded in §38.9):
1. **Weighted-Voronoi merge.** Cluster the post-branch Diracs into `≤P` cells; replace each cell by a single Dirac at its weight-barycenter with summed weight. This preserves total mass (§38.6) and the first moment exactly; it perturbs the **second moment** by the within-cell variance, injecting an `O(\text{diam}_{\text{cell}}^2)` per-reduction error — analogous to a grid `O(dx²)` floor but *adaptive* (cells dense where mass concentrates).
2. **Gaussian-smoothed background.** Replace the long-time tail by a moment-matched Gaussian, evolved in closed form (the §38.7 Brownian variance accumulation `Δσ² = 2aτ` per step is exact), keeping only the near-field as explicit particles.

**NORMATIVE consequence.** The reduction error is the *price* of escaping `4ⁿ`; the variance claim of §50.6 must therefore be **measured against this realized error**, NOT against the unreduced ideal. A *randomized* reduction (e.g. systematic resampling) re-introduces estimator variance — which is exactly why `G_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE` is a **go/no-go**: deterministic ¼,¼,½ branching + a *deterministic* reduction is what gives the quasi-MC-like low-discrepancy structure; if a randomized reduction is needed, the low-variance thesis is at risk.

> *NORMATIVE (d-dim reduction).* `R_P` MUST cluster in **all `d` coordinates** (product-bin or
> k-d barycenter), preserving **per-axis** first moments on every axis. Binning along a single
> axis collapses off-axis structure and is non-conformant. `R_P` is applied **after each axis
> sub-step** of the §50.2 sweep to bound the working set to `O(d·P_cap)` (defeating the `3^d`
> blow-up); applying it once per full step incurs `3^d·P` peak memory and forfeits the H-MEM
> headline.

### §50.5 — The variance claim (NORMATIVE library — TO BE MEASURED, not assumed)

The defensible, unique hypothesis (research §2.1): the *deterministic* ¼,¼,½ branching of (50.3) is a **low-discrepancy (quasi-MC-like) quadrature** of the heat kernel, so the gridless estimator has **strictly lower variance than a naive Monte-Carlo random walk** of the same particle budget `P`. This is graded **C** in the literature (closest published analogue: time-splitting + QMC for Fokker-Planck, grade B) and is the make-or-break experiment. **It is asserted as a hypothesis to be MEASURED by `G_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE`, never assumed true in any proof.** If falsified, Shift C reverts to research-only (ADR-0155 Consequences; research §5.3 Phase 2). The comparison MUST be equal-information: same budget `P`, same replications `R`, same functional, same closed-form truth, and a **shared common-random-number** quantization of `δ_0` consumed identically by both the deterministic and the MC estimator. Comparing the deterministic estimator's initial-condition sensitivity against the MC sampling noise is a non-conformant apples-to-oranges measurement and is explicitly forbidden.

### §50.6 — Acceptance gates (NORMATIVE — PLANNED)

- **`G_GRIDLESS_DIM_SCALING`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`, MEASURED — d=2 PASS, d≥4 INTRINSIC LIMIT): linear anisotropic heat / Black-Scholes basket on `ℝ^d`, `d ∈ {2,4,6,8,10}`, evolved by the deterministic-branching particle evolver vs the dense `GridND` (where it fits) and `SmolyakGridND` (D≤6). Three conjunctive thresholds: (i) **accuracy** — sup-error vs closed-form / high-`n` reference `< 5e-3` at each `d`; (ii) **cost scaling** — the `log`-`log` OLS slope of per-step cost vs `d` is `≤ 1.1` (near-linear in `d`), contrasted against the grid's exponential `≈ d·log N`; (iii) **memory** — peak memory grows **sub-exponentially in `d`** (the H-MEM flagship axis — the real win). **Sign convention (NORMATIVE):** the cost-scaling slope is taken with respect to `log d`; a value `≤ 1.1` PASSES (smaller = closer to dimension-independent; the *opposite* sign direction from the order-of-accuracy gates G24/§47.5, which are `≥` because larger order is better — stated explicitly to avoid a sign trap). The accuracy functional and reference MUST depend on **all `d` axes** (e.g. product char-fn `∏_j cos(ξ_j x_j)` vs `∏_j e^{−Tξ_j² a_j}` with not-all-equal `a_j, ξ_j`); the five `d`-estimates must be mutually distinct (a constant-across-`d` result signals dimensional collapse). The cost-scaling slope MUST be taken over a cost metric that genuinely grows with `d` before reduction (pre-reduction branch work `3^d`, or the budget `P_cap(d)` needed to hold accuracy) — a cap fixed independent of `d` makes the slope ≡0 trivially and is non-conformant.
- **`G_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE`** (go/no-go sub-check, `slow-tests`, MEASURED — NO-GO 1.417× < 2× gate): at a fixed particle budget `P`, the deterministic-branching estimator's empirical variance MUST be **strictly below** an MC random-walk estimator of the same `P` (target **≥ 2× reduction**), and within a documented factor of a Sobol-QMC baseline. **This sub-check FIRED as NO-GO** (measured MSE ratio 1.417× at d=2, fair CRN comparison, 2026-06-09) — the "structured = low-variance" thesis is NOT confirmed ≥2×; Shift C ships NARROW and **Shift B (`ReverseChernoff`) is the v9.0.0 headline** (see §50 STATUS admonition and ADR-0155 Amendment).
- **`T_GRIDLESS_*`** (NORMATIVE numeric+sympy oracle — ADR-0155, `scripts/gridless_kit.py`, **PASS 3/3**): sub-checks proving (1) **generator consistency of the particle map** — the single-step particle map (50.3), expanded on a 2nd-order Taylor stencil with `f(x), f'(x), f''(x)` as abstract symbols, reproduces the intended generator `S(τ)f = f + τ·Lf + o(τ)` with `L = a∂² + b∂' + c` to order `τ¹` (the ¼/¼/½ branch weights and the `h = 2√(aτ)`, `k = 2bτ` step sizes are verified to first order), PLUS a coefficient-sum sanity check (`¼+¼+½ = 1`) on the dual-pairing weights. **Honest scope (NORMATIVE, v9.1.0 correction):** this is a *generator-consistency to O(τ)* proof plus a coefficient-sum check; it is NOT a symbolic verification of the adjoint identity `⟨f, S*(τ)δ_x⟩ = (S(τ)f)(x)` over a non-trivial `f`-class (that identity holds by definition of `S*` as the §38.2 adjoint). The oracle **re-derives the §38 generator stencil inline** — it does NOT import or reuse `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS` code (the earlier "reuses … machinery" wording was a code-level overstatement, corrected here; the reuse is conceptual — same §38 generator — only). (2) **mass conservation** — total weight reweights by `∏(1 + τc)` exactly (§38.6); (3) **moment match of the reduction** — `R_P` preserves mass and first moment, second-moment error bounded by within-cell variance (§50.4) — this is a PROVED *single-merge, per-cluster local* identity; the *propagated, uniform-in-(n,d)* `R_P` bound is OPEN (§50.7) and was empirically refuted in high d. Prints exactly `T_GRIDLESS PASS` / `T_GRIDLESS FAIL: <reason>`. Pure symbolic — runs in the `test-fast` sympy sweep without `slow-tests`; failure BLOCKS v9.0.0+ release per the ADR-0086 RELEASE_BLOCKING-for-math-fidelity precedent.

### §50.7 — Limitations, negative results, and resolution (NORMATIVE)

- **Bounded `d ≤ ~10`, linear coefficient only (NARROW particle ship).** High-`d` (d>10), nonlinear,
  and genuinely variable-coefficient gridless evolution via the **particle** form are RESEARCH-TRACK.
- **INTRINSIC LIMIT: spatial-merge reduction is O(m^d); curse re-enters the reduction grid (measured
  2026-06-09).** ANY spatial-merge particle-reduction that needs `m` bins per axis to hold accuracy
  must hold a working set that grows at least as fast as the number of occupied cells, which is
  `O(m^d)` for an isotropic `d`-dimensional distribution. Both the product-bin and k-d-barycenter
  forms (§50.4) are subject to this: at fixed accuracy, `P_cap(d)` must grow to compensate the
  `d·O(cell_diam²)` per-step reduction floor (each of `d` sub-steps injects an `O(cell_diam²)`
  reduction error). The measurements confirm this: d=2 passes with moderate cap (validated envelope);
  d=3 needs 8× the d=2 cap; d≥4 collapses in accuracy (errs 9.75e-2 to 7.05e-1) regardless of cap
  because the required bin count exceeds the available budget. This is not a tunable implementation bug
  — it is the curse of dimensionality re-entering through the reduction grid. The validated envelope is
  **d=2**. The low-variance thesis (§50.5) was not confirmed ≥2× under fair CRN comparison even at d=2
  (measured ratio 1.417×). Together these mean: *the spatial-merge particle primitive is the wrong
  primitive for the high-d headline claim*.
- **THE RESOLUTION IS THE TENSOR-TRAIN CARRIER (§52).** The INTRINSIC LIMIT above is NOT a failure of
  the Chernoff evolver — it is a failure of the particle representation as the state carrier. The
  breakthrough (§52, ADR-0159): holding the state as a low-rank TT and evolving it under the
  rank-preserving per-axis Chernoff shift (Kazeev–Khoromskij Grade A, §52.2) escapes the exponential
  curse for the linear diagonal-A (Gaussian) class (Rohrbach–Dolgov–Grasedyck–Scheichl Gaussian rank
  cap r ≤ d/2, §52.4). This is the correct resolution of the §50 TRIZ ФП. The four prior particle-side
  reframes and the §52 TT principle are **complementary** and **consistent**: together they close the
  problem — the escape is through the TT representation; the curse is intrinsic to the solution's rank
  for the dense-correlation case and cannot be escaped by any representation.
- **Path-space RQMC — residual research-track direction (ADR-0158).** For the non-Gaussian /
  dense-correlation regime where TT rank blows up, path-space RQMC (Sobol + Brownian-bridge over the
  `n·d` trajectory dimensions) remains a candidate. ADR-0158 records the design; the grade-C Corput
  data point lost to plain MC; proper Sobol + Brownian-bridge is untested.
- **General `4ⁿ`-reduction theory.** A sharp error bound for `R_P` uniform in `n` and `d` is open.
- **Prior-art re-confirmation.** No paper iterating a Chernoff product formula on a particle ensemble
  was found (gap graded C). The Festschrift arXiv:2508.18650 must be re-fetched.
- **Smoothness floor.** The kernel quadrature needs `C²_b` data (§32.3); rough payoffs degrade the
  inherited order.

### §50.8 — References

- M. Hutzenthaler, A. Jentzen, T. Kruse, et al., *Multilevel Picard approximations of high-dimensional semilinear parabolic PDEs* (polynomial complexity, dims to 10,000). **SIAM J. Numer. Anal.** DOI [10.1137/17M1157015](https://doi.org/10.1137/17M1157015); arXiv:1708.03223. — **A**, the strongest competitor; C competes on memory + determinism + reproducibility, NOT asymptotic rate (research §2.5 R-C2).
- W. E, J. Han, A. Jentzen, *Solving high-dimensional PDEs using deep learning*, **PNAS** 115(34):8505–8510 (2018). DOI [10.1073/pnas.1718942115](https://doi.org/10.1073/pnas.1718942115). — **A** (deep BSDE, the data-driven lane C deliberately does NOT enter).
- P. Henry-Labordère, N. Touzi et al., *Branching diffusion representation for nonlinear Cauchy problems*, **AIHP** 55(1) 2019; arXiv:1801.08794. — **A** (the random-walk branching baseline C's *deterministic* branching is compared against).
- *Quasi-Monte Carlo algorithms for diffusion equations in high dimensions* (time-splitting + QMC; variance reduction), **J. Comput. Appl. Math.** ScienceDirect S0378475404002587. — **B**, the closest published analogue to C's variance claim (§50.5).
- I. D. Remizov, *The method of Chernoff approximation* (survey), arXiv:1905.07309. — **A (survey)**; quasi-Feynman "multiple integrals of infinite multiplicity".
- Galkin-Remizov 2025, *Upper and lower estimates for rate of convergence in the Chernoff product formula*, **Israel J. Math.** 265, 929-943, Theorem 4 — the forward Chernoff function dualised in §38.3, reused here.
- **Internal**: math §38 / ADR-0107 (`AdjointFokkerPlanckChernoff` on `M(ℝ^d)`, `T_ADJOINT_FP_TIGHTNESS` 6/6 PASS, `MeasureState<F,D>` — the embryo evolver); §32 / ADR-0081 (`AnisotropicShiftChernoffND` d-D shift; Backend-E fallback note); §44 / ADR-0123 (`SmolyakGridND` D=6, the deterministic high-`d` baseline benchmarked against); ADR-0155 (Shift C); ADR-0154 (v9.0.0 umbrella, third S-curve).
