## §51 — Reverse-mode AD over the Chernoff product via binomial checkpointing — `ReverseChernoff` (v9.0.0 SHIP-TRACK, ADR-0156, NORMATIVE library; CITATION mathematics — third S-curve, R2)

> **§51 STATUS — v9.0.0 SHIPPED FORWARD-DUAL ONLY; v9.1.0 makes it GENUINELY reverse (ADR-0156 Amendment 1; gate corrected in Amendment 2).**
> **v9.1.0 Amendment 2 (2026-06-10):** the original v9.1.0 §51.4 "0-ULP K=1 cross-mode parity" gate was
> SELF-DEFEATING — 0-ULP agreement between a genuine reverse VJP and a forward JVP is impossible in
> floating point (different reduction orders), so the only way to pass it was to make "reverse" run the
> forward ops (the tautology it forbade). Phase-2 engineering was cornered into a forward-mode JVP
> relabelled "reverse" (`reverse_sweep.rs::backward_sweep_k1`). Amendment 2 (i) replaces leg (ii) with a
> TIGHT RELATIVE tolerance `< 1e-12` (justified `C·n·ε`); (ii) confines 0-ULP to same-algorithm
> cross-platform parity (`G_BINDING_REVERSE_AD_PARITY`); (iii) adds `G_REVERSE_AD_STRUCTURE` (mutation
> oracle proving `Jᵀ` is load-bearing) so a forward-tangent dodge FAILS; (iv) clarifies that transport
> terms live in `b_k=∂F/∂θ` (computed by the dual `step_jacobian_col`), NOT in `Jᵀ` (linear-in-state ⇒
> plain transpose stencil) — removing the obstruction that drove the dodge. **VERDICT: genuine
> reverse-mode is ACHIEVABLE for the NARROW constant-a / linear-Magnus scope.**
> **HONEST CORRECTION (2026-06-10, v9.1.0):** the v9.0.0 public gradient API `value_and_grad_k1`
> computed the gradient by running the **forward-mode `Dual<F>` pass** (§46), NOT a reverse/adjoint
> backward sweep; the genuine reverse machinery (`recompute_segment`, `step_jacobian_col`, the
> cotangent recursion `λ_{k-1}=Fᵀλ_k`) shipped as `#[allow(dead_code)]` and was never wired. As a
> consequence the v9.0.0 "0-ULP cross-mode parity" gate was tautological (`reverse_grad ==
> forward_dual` because both were the SAME forward-dual computation), and **no K>1 gradient shipped**.
> The gradient *value* was correct (FD-validated); the *method* claim "reverse-mode AD" was not honored.
>
> **v9.1.0 (this section, NORMATIVE):** the public path becomes the GENUINE cotangent backward sweep
> over checkpointed segments (the resolution already designed in §51.1–51.3, now WIRED), AND a **K>1**
> multi-parameter gradient computed in a SINGLE backward pass — this is the actual capability tier over
> v8 §46 forward dual-AD (which costs `O(K)` forward passes). The forward-dual pass is retained ONLY as
> the **independent** 0-ULP parity reference (§51.4, now a real cross-mode check between two distinct
> computations, not `x==x`). Gates: `G_REVERSE_AD_GRADIENT` (FD + genuine-reverse-vs-forward-dual
> 0-ULP), `G_REVERSE_AD_CHECKPOINT` (O(√n) memory), **`G_REVERSE_AD_ADVANTAGE`** (NEW — asserts reverse
> is O(1)-in-K vs forward-dual O(K); §51.9). Oracle **`T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE` is corrected to 3/3** — the
> NEW sub-check (3) proves the non-vacuous adjoint/VJP identity `⟨v, Ju⟩ = ⟨Jᵀv, u⟩` on explicit
> symbolic `J, Jᵀ` AND `Jᵀ == transpose(J)` entrywise (§51.9). The transpose-exactness guarantee is
> honestly SCOPED to the linear / truncated-Magnus family for which §42 proves it (`T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE`);
> variable-coefficient/nonlinear kernels must re-establish it per-kernel (research §3.5 R-B3).

### §51.1 — Motivation (NORMATIVE library scope)

The v8.0.0 differentiability axis shipped **forward-mode** dual-AD (§46, `Dual<F>`), §42 transpose-exactness (`T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE`), and §43 adjoint-state sensitivity. Forward-mode costs `O(K)` for `K` parameters. **Reverse-mode** delivers the full gradient in `O(1)` trajectory passes — the right tool for many-parameter calibration and ML-training-through-a-PDE-layer. The unused resource **R2**: because `F(τ)` has **no implicit solver** (pure shift-and-scale), the adjoint of the trajectory `(F(τ))ⁿ` is the **transposed product of the same steps**, algebraically exact — unlike Neural-ODE / Diffrax continuous adjoints, which either re-solve an implicit backward equation (approximate) or store the whole forward trajectory (`O(n·state)` memory).

### §51.2 — The trajectory transpose (CITATION — §42 transpose-exactness)

Let `F(τ)` be one Chernoff step with linear part represented by the bounded operator `F` on the discrete state. The forward trajectory is `u_n = F^n u_0`. For a scalar loss `J = ℓ(u_n)`, reverse-mode propagates the adjoint (cotangent) `λ_k := (∂J/∂u_k)^⊤` backward by the **transposed step**:
$$
\lambda_n = (\nabla_{u}\ell)(u_n), \qquad \lambda_{k-1} = F^{\!\top}\,\lambda_k \quad (k = n, n{-}1, \dots, 1), \tag{51.1}
$$
so the parameter gradient accumulates as `∂J/∂θ = Σ_{k} λ_k^⊤ (∂F/∂θ) u_{k-1}`. **§42 proves `F^⊤` is algebraically exact** (not a numerical adjoint) for the degree-4 truncated-Magnus map (`T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE`): the transpose of a shift `τ_{+a}` is the shift `τ_{−a}`, the transpose of a scalar multiply is itself, and the transpose of the interpolation stencil is its (sparse, banded) matrix transpose — all available without any solve, because R2 guarantees there is no solver to invert. **Sign convention (NORMATIVE):** the backward recursion (51.1) runs `k` *decreasing*; `F^⊤` uses the *negated* shift vectors of the forward step (transpose of `τ_{+a}` is `τ_{−a}`), the mirror of the §50.2 push-forward sign relation under the same §38.2 dual pairing.

### §51.3 — Binomial checkpointing for `O(√n)` memory (CITATION — Griewank-Walther; Diffrax)

A classic Wengert-list **tape** would store all `n` intermediate states (`O(n·state)` memory) and needs dynamic allocation incompatible with the suckless posture. Instead, store every `√n`-th state as a **checkpoint** and recompute each `√n`-length segment forward on demand during the backward sweep:
$$
\text{peak memory} = O(\sqrt{n}\cdot\text{state}), \qquad \text{recompute cost} = O(n)\ \text{extra forward steps}. \tag{51.2}
$$
This is the Griewank-Walther `revolve` / Diffrax recommended binomial-checkpoint scheme; it is `alloc`-only (a `Vec` of `O(√n)` checkpoints), `no_std`-clean, and requires **no external autodiff crate** (respects Override #1's ≤3-direct-dep budget). It is the resolution of the TRIZ ФП "the trajectory must be stored AND not stored": the trajectory *recomputes itself* because the solver-free step (R2) is cheap to replay (ADR-0156, research §3.3).

### §51.4 — Cross-mode parity to §46 (NORMATIVE library — CORRECTED v9.1.0 Amendment 2)

> **HONEST CORRECTION (2026-06-10, v9.1.0 Amendment 2 — the gate fixed itself into the tautology it forbade).**
> The v9.1.0 (pre-Amendment-2) §51.4 demanded that for `K=1` the reverse-mode gradient match the
> forward-mode `Dual<F>` gradient to **0 ULP** "by the adjoint identity, not by shared code." **This
> requirement is mathematically impossible for two genuinely independent floating-point paths and is
> self-defeating.** A reverse VJP (`g = Σ_k ⟨λ_k, b_k⟩` with backward `λ_{k-1}=Jᵀλ_k`) and a forward
> JVP (`g = ⟨w, t_n⟩` with forward `t_k = J·t_{k-1}+b_k`) are equal in **exact** arithmetic (the adjoint
> identity), but they execute **different operation sequences with different summation orders**, so in IEEE-754
> they agree only to `O(n)·κ·ε` relative (≈ 1e-15…1e-13), **NOT to 0 ULP**. The ONLY way to satisfy a
> 0-ULP cross-mode gate is to make the "reverse" path run the *same* forward float ops — i.e. the
> tautology the clause was written to forbid. The Phase-2 engineer was thereby cornered into a
> forward-mode JVP relabelled "reverse" (`reverse_sweep.rs::backward_sweep_k1`: forward `k=1..n` loop,
> tangent accumulator, `Dual.tangent` extraction — no `Jᵀ`, no cotangent). **Root cause: the gate, not
> the engineer.** Amendment 2 corrects the gate below.

**(i) Reverse vs finite-difference — KEPT.** Reverse-mode gradient matches a central / Richardson
finite-difference reference to `< 1e-9` (relative). This is the primary correctness leg (unchanged).

**(ii) Reverse vs forward-mode `Dual<F>` — CORRECTED to a TIGHT RELATIVE tolerance.** For `K=1`,
reverse-mode (the GENUINE cotangent backward sweep, §51.9) matches forward-mode dual-AD (§46) to
**`< 1e-12` (relative)**, NOT 0 ULP. **Justification of the bound (NORMATIVE).** The two computations
realise the same exact derivative through different reduction orders; the cross-mode discrepancy is
bounded by `C·n·κ·ε` where `n` is the step count (`≤ 1024` in the gates), `κ` the modest condition
number of the symmetric stencil, and `ε ≈ 2.22e-16` (f64). With `n ≤ 1024` this is `≈ 1e-13`, so
`1e-12` leaves ~1 order of safety margin above the genuine-agreement floor while staying **three
orders tighter than the FD leg (i)** — it is a real cross-mode check, not slack. (For non-f64 `F`,
scale the bound by `F`'s machine epsilon: gate `< C·n·ε_F`, default `C·n ≤ 4096`.)

**Where 0-ULP genuinely belongs (NORMATIVE).** The 0-ULP bit-exact culture (`G_BINDING_GREEKS_PARITY`)
is preserved ONLY for **same-algorithm cross-platform** checks: `G_BINDING_REVERSE_AD_PARITY` MUST keep
Rust-core ≡ PyO3 ≡ WASM to **0 ULP**, because those run the *identical* reverse sweep on different
runtimes (same op sequence ⇒ bit-reproducible). 0-ULP is the correct gate for *reproducibility of one
computation*, the WRONG gate for *agreement of two different computations*.

**NORMATIVE anti-tautology clause (RETAINED, strengthened — STRUCTURAL not bit-exact).** Leg (ii) is
meaningful only if the two sides are independent computations: the reverse side MUST originate from the
cotangent backward sweep (§51.9: forward checkpoints + seed `λ_n=2(u_n−target)` + backward
`λ_{k-1}=Jᵀλ_k` via `apply_transpose_step` + parameter accumulation `g=Σ_k⟨λ_k,b_k⟩` via
`step_jacobian_col`); the forward side is §46 dual JVP. A forward-mode-tangent implementation
relabelled "reverse" (the v9.0.0 and Phase-2 defect) is NON-CONFORMANT and MUST FAIL the gate. Because
a tolerance gate alone cannot detect the dodge (a correct forward JVP also passes leg (i)+(ii)),
conformance is enforced **structurally** by §51.6 `G_REVERSE_AD_STRUCTURE` (the reverse path provably
applies `Jᵀ` and runs `k=n→1`) and by `G_REVERSE_AD_ADVANTAGE` (§51.9: forward-tangent needs `O(K)`
passes and FAILS the K-scaling gate). The reverse gradient MUST originate from the backward sweep; any
path that routes through forward-dual tangent propagation VOIDS conformance.

### §51.5 — REUSE boundary and honest scope (NORMATIVE library — NARROW)

Reverse-mode reuses §42 (`F^⊤` exactness), §43 (adjoint-state accumulation), and §46 (`Dual<F>` for the per-step parameter Jacobian `∂F/∂θ`). **Transpose-exactness is proven only for the truncated-Magnus / linear family** (§42 scope). For variable-coefficient or nonlinear kernels the clean transpose is NOT guaranteed and MUST be re-established per-kernel or the kernel is documented OUT of reverse-AD scope for v9.0.0 (research §3.5 R-B3). The integration surface is **PyO3 / WASM `value_and_grad`**; a PyTorch/JAX custom-op is downstream glue kept OUT of the `no_std` core (research §3.4).

### §51.6 — Acceptance gates (NORMATIVE — PLANNED)

- **`G_REVERSE_AD_GRADIENT`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`, PLANNED): end-to-end gradient of `J(θ) = ‖(F_θ(τ))ⁿ u₀ − target‖²` w.r.t. a `K`-vector `θ` (diffusion coeff, drift, payoff knot). Two conjunctive thresholds: (i) reverse-mode gradient matches a central finite-difference reference to `< 1e-9` (relative); (ii) for `K=1`, reverse-mode matches the **forward-mode `Dual<F>` gradient (§46) to `< 1e-12` (relative)** — a TIGHT cross-mode check between two genuinely independent float paths, NOT 0 ULP (CORRECTED §51.4 Amendment 2; the prior 0-ULP demand was self-defeating). At least one kernel MUST run on the default `Grid1D::new` (SepticHermite) grid (mirrors the §46.7 anti-dodge clause).
- **`G_REVERSE_AD_STRUCTURE`** (NORMATIVE structural conformance, `test-fast`, NEW v9.1.0 Amendment 2): proves the reverse path genuinely runs the cotangent recursion (not a forward-tangent relabel). Two sub-checks: **(a) transpose-is-load-bearing (mutation oracle)** — replacing the per-step transpose `apply_transpose_step` with the identity map MUST change the computed gradient by `> 1e-6` relative (if it does not, `Jᵀ` is not actually applied — the forward-tangent dodge); **(b) backward-direction witness** — the implementation MUST consume `apply_transpose_step` and `step_jacobian_col` and walk `k=n→1` (verified by an internal call-order assertion or by the type signature requiring both adjoint primitives). A forward-mode-JVP implementation (forward `k=1..n` loop, no `Jᵀ`) FAILS sub-check (a). RELEASE_BLOCKING; runs in `test-fast` (small `n`, cheap).
- **`G_REVERSE_AD_CHECKPOINT`** (memory sub-check, `slow-tests`, PLANNED): peak heap allocation during the backward pass grows `O(√n)` (binomial checkpointing), NOT `O(n)` (tape), verified by a counting global allocator over `n ∈ {64, 256, 1024}` (reuse the `G_DUAL_ZERO_ALLOC` harness). **Sign convention (NORMATIVE):** the gate fits `log(peak_mem)` vs `log n` and requires slope `≤ 0.6` (ideal `0.5`); a value `≤ 0.6` PASSES (smaller = better memory scaling — the opposite direction from the order gates).
- **`T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE`** (NORMATIVE numeric+sympy oracle — ADR-0156, `scripts/reverse_transpose_kit.py`, **PASS 2/2**): extends `T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE` (§42) from one step to the full trajectory — verifies `((F(τ))ⁿ)^⊤ = (F^⊤)ⁿ` symbolically (transpose of a product = reversed product of transposes) and that the per-step transpose negates shift vectors and transposes the banded interpolation stencil. Prints exactly `T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE PASS` / `T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE FAIL: <reason>`. Pure symbolic — runs in `test-fast`; failure BLOCKS v9.0.0+ release.

### §51.9 — GENUINE reverse-mode wiring + K>1 + advantage gate (v9.1.0 NORMATIVE — ADR-0156 Amendment 1)

**The public gradient path is the cotangent backward sweep (NORMATIVE).** `ReverseChernoff::value_and_grad(τ, n, u₀, target, θ ∈ ℝ^K) → (J, ∇J ∈ ℝ^K)` MUST be computed by:
1. forward pass with `⌈√n⌉` binomial checkpointing (§51.3), loss `J = ‖u_n − target‖²`, seed cotangent `λ_n = ∂J/∂u_n = 2(u_n − target)`;
2. backward sweep `k = n…1` (**`k` strictly decreasing** — the witness of genuine reverse-mode): (a) replay `u_{k-1}` from the nearest checkpoint via `recompute_segment` (bit-exact); (b) accumulate the parameter gradient `∇J[p] += ⟨λ_k, b_k^{(p)}⟩` where `b_k^{(p)} := (∂F/∂θ_p)(u_{k-1})` for each `p∈0..K`; (c) propagate the cotangent `λ_{k-1} = Jᵀ λ_k` via `apply_transpose_step` (§51.2, negated shift; **`Jᵀ = J` for constant-a `DiffusionChernoff` — the stencil is symmetric**).

**Transport terms live in `b_k`, NOT in `Jᵀ` (NORMATIVE clarification — resolves the Phase-2 obstruction).** Because `F_θ` is **linear in its state argument** (`(F_θ v)_i = Σ_j J_{ij}(θ) v_j`, an interpolation-stencil mat-vec), the **state Jacobian** `∂F/∂u = J(θ)` is *exactly* the banded shift-and-scale matrix — it contains **no transport terms**, and its transpose `Jᵀ` (negated shift + transposed stencil, §51.2) is what the cotangent recursion (c) applies. The **θ-dependent sample-position transport** (`h₀(θ)=2√(θτ)`, `∂(F_θ u)_i/∂θ = W_1[u'(x{+}h₀){−}u'(x{−}h₀)]\,h₀'(θ)+W_2[\dots]\,h₀₃'(θ)`) appears **only in the parameter sensitivity** `b_k^{(p)} = (∂F/∂θ_p)(u_{k-1})` — step (b). The Phase-2 engineer's claim that `apply_f(τ,&t)` cannot capture transport was TRUE but MISPLACED: transport belongs to `b_k`, never to `Jᵀλ`. Conflating the two is what drove the forward-dual dodge. The correct design captures transport in `b_k` via one §46 dual step holding the state fixed (below); `Jᵀ` has no transport and is the plain transpose stencil (delegating to the symmetric `apply_f` for constant-a).

**`step_jacobian_col` contract (REPAIRED — computes `b_k^{(p)}`, transport-complete).** For parameter `θ_p`, `step_jacobian_col` MUST: build a dual state `ŝ = {value: u_{k-1}, tangent: 0}` (**zero state tangent** — the state is held fixed), apply one dual step of the kernel **seeded with `∂/∂θ_p` in the differentiated coefficient** (e.g. `a(x) = Dual::variable(θ)` for the constant-a diffusivity; `τ` carries **no** tangent — `tau_dual = Dual::constant(τ)`), and extract the output `.tangent` field, which equals `b_k^{(p)} = (∂F/∂θ_p)(u_{k-1})` with the sample-position transport differentiated automatically by the dual arithmetic through `h₀(θ)`. **Repair of the shipped stub:** the v9.0.0 `step_jacobian_col` docstring said "tangent seeded 1 in `tau_dual`" — that seeds `∂/∂τ`, the WRONG parameter; the seed MUST be on the differentiated parameter `θ_p` (in the kernel's coefficient closure), not on `τ`. For `K>1`, one seeded dual kernel per `θ_p` (or a `K`-component dual); each yields `b_k^{(p)}` reusing the SAME checkpointed `u_{k-1}` — no extra forward trajectory. This is the resource that makes the backward pass `O(1)`-in-trajectory-passes regardless of `K`.

A forward-dual / forward-tangent gradient is FORBIDDEN as the public reverse path (it is the v9.0.0 *and* Phase-2 defect — a forward `k=1..n` tangent accumulator with no `Jᵀ`); forward-dual is retained ONLY as the §51.4 leg-(ii) parity reference (now a `< 1e-12` tolerance check, not 0 ULP). **K>1 in ONE backward pass** is the capability tier over §46: forward dual-AD costs `O(K)` trajectory passes (one tangent seed per parameter); the reverse sweep propagates the single cotangent `λ` in `O(1)` trajectory passes independent of `K`, accumulating all `K` parameter gradients `⟨λ_k, b_k^{(p)}⟩` in the single backward walk, at `O(√n)` memory. **The genuine-reverse requirement binds where it matters — K>1:** `G_REVERSE_AD_ADVANTAGE` (below) is the gate that truly distinguishes reverse (O(1)-in-K passes) from forward (O(K)); a forward-tangent implementation needs `K` forward passes and FAILS it. **If `K=1` is exercised, it MUST route through the SAME backward-sweep machinery** (seed `λ_n`, apply `Jᵀ`, accumulate `⟨λ_k,b_k⟩`) — NOT a special-cased forward path. There is no separate `value_and_grad_k1` forward shortcut; `K=1` is `value_and_grad` with a length-1 `θ`.

**Corrected `T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE` (3/3, NON-VACUOUS, RELEASE_BLOCKING).** Sub-checks (1) product-transpose factorisation and (2) per-step transpose structure are KEPT. **NEW sub-check (3) — the structurally-independent VJP oracle:** for the discrete Chernoff Jacobian `J = ∂(Fu)/∂u` (banded shift-and-scale matrix), construct `J` and `Jᵀ` as explicit sympy matrices and verify, for arbitrary symbolic vectors `v, u`, that `(J u)·v − u·(Jᵀ v) ≡ 0` (the adjoint identity `⟨v, Ju⟩ = ⟨Jᵀv, u⟩`) AND that `Jᵀ` equals the entrywise matrix transpose of `J` (so the implemented `apply_transpose_step` realises the true adjoint: negated shift + transposed stencil + scalar-invariant). This is non-vacuous because the LHS is built from the forward matrix and the RHS from the transpose the backward sweep actually applies — they agree only if the transpose is correct, not by construction. `scripts/reverse_transpose_kit.py` prints `T_REVERSE_TRANSPOSE PASS (3/3 …)`.

**`G_REVERSE_AD_ADVANTAGE`** (NEW, RELEASE_BLOCKING for the capability claim, `slow-tests`): for fixed `n` and `K ∈ {1,4,16,64}`, measure step-application count for (a) the reverse sweep and (b) forward dual-AD. **PASS iff** the cotangent-propagation work of the reverse sweep is `O(1)` in `K` while forward dual-AD is `O(K)` — concretely, `ratio(K) = forward_work(K) / reverse_traj_passes` grows ≥ linearly, gate `ratio(64)/ratio(1) ≥ 8` (conservative slope floor). This gate FAILS on the v9.0.0 forward-dual relabel and is the gate that actually asserts the new tier. **Sign convention (NORMATIVE):** larger ratio = better (more advantage), `≥` threshold — the order-gate direction, distinct from the §52.5 / §51.6 memory-slope `≤` gates.

### §51.7 — Limitations and future work

- **Linear / Magnus family only** for proven transpose-exactness (§51.5). Variable-coefficient/nonlinear re-proof is research-track.
- **No PyTorch/JAX custom-op in core.** The mainstream-SciML ecosystem is the moat-breaker (research §3.5 R-B2); the honest niche is embedded/edge/HFT differentiable control. Downstream glue is out of scope.
- **Checkpoint schedule fixed at `√n`.** An optimal Griewank `revolve` schedule (memory-bounded, recompute-minimal) is deferred; the `√n` schedule is the simple correct default.

### §51.8 — References

- A. Griewank, A. Walther, *Algorithm 799: revolve — an implementation of checkpointing for the reverse or adjoint mode of computational differentiation*, **ACM TOMS** 26(1):19–45 (2000). DOI [10.1145/347837.347846](https://doi.org/10.1145/347837.347846) — the `O(√n)`-memory binomial checkpointing of §51.3.
- R. T. Q. Chen, Y. Rubanova, J. Bettencourt, D. Duvenaud, *Neural Ordinary Differential Equations*, **NeurIPS** 2018 — the O(1)-memory continuous adjoint that is *approximate* (re-solves backward); §50 is exact at `O(√n)` because R2 gives an exact transpose. — **A**
- P. Kidger, *Diffrax* adjoints (binomial checkpointing; discretize- vs optimize-then-discretize). https://docs.kidger.site/diffrax/api/adjoints/ — **A**, the checkpointing strategy reused.
- T. Matsubara et al., *Symplectic Adjoint Method for Exact Gradient of Neural ODE with Minimal Memory*, **NeurIPS** 2021; arXiv:2102.09750. — **B** (exact-gradient-at-low-memory precedent).
- **Internal**: math §42 / ADR (transpose-exactness, `T_MAGNUS_TRANSPOSE` — extended here); §43 (adjoint-state sensitivity — accumulation reused); §46 / ADR-0133 (`Dual<F>` forward AD, `G_DUAL_AD_GRADIENT`/`G_DUAL_ZERO_ALLOC` PASS — the cross-mode 0-ULP parity partner of §51.4); `G_BINDING_GREEKS_PARITY` (0-ULP binding-parity culture reused); ADR-0156 (Shift B); ADR-0154 (v9.0.0 umbrella, third S-curve).

### §51.10 — Multi-parameter (K>1) reverse-AD via piecewise-region coefficients (NORMATIVE — ADR-0177, issue #1)

> **STATUS — v9.x extension.** This makes `value_and_grad(τ, n, u₀, target, θ ∈ ℝ^K)` genuinely
> K-vector (lifts the §51.9 / ADR-0172 K=1-only restriction). It does NOT alter §51.9 for K=1:
> one region = all of Ω reproduces the §51.9 path **byte-identically**. NORMATIVE library.

**The ill-posedness ADR-0172 named, and its resolution.** For a single scalar `a(x) ≡ θ` the K
seeds coincide and the backward sweep broadcasts one gradient into all K slots — the *correct*
value of an ill-posed question. K>1 is made **well-posed in space** (ADR-0177, resolution in
space) by partitioning the grid DoF into K disjoint regions and giving each its own coefficient.

**Per-region coefficient model (NORMATIVE).** Partition the `N_grid` nodes into K disjoint regions
`Ω = ⊔_{r=0}^{K-1} Ω_r` via a DoF-aligned map `ρ : {0..N_grid} → {0..K}` (`ρ(i)=r ⟺ node i ∈ Ω_r`).
The diffusion coefficient is the single piecewise-constant function

    a(x_i) = Σ_{r=0}^{K-1} θ_r · 𝟙_{Ω_r}(x_i) = θ_{ρ(i)} .

This is ONE `DiffusionChernoff` (one `a(x)`, built via `with_closure`), so `J = ∂(Fu)/∂u` is the
same banded self-adjoint stencil **inside each region** and `Jᵀ = F` (§51.2) is unchanged — the
indicator is piecewise-constant, it perturbs values, not the state-Jacobian symmetry. The
`ChernoffFunction` trait signature is untouched (CRITICAL: 56 dependents, ADR-0177).

**Per-region Jacobian column (NORMATIVE).** For parameter `θ_r`, the per-step parameter sensitivity

    b_k^{(r)} := (∂F/∂θ_r)(u_{k-1}),     supp(b_k^{(r)}) ⊆ Ω_r ,

is computed by ONE dual step (§46, `step_jacobian_col`) whose coefficient closure seeds
`Dual::variable(θ_r)` on nodes `i ∈ Ω_r` and `Dual::constant(θ_{ρ(i)})` elsewhere (state held at
zero tangent, `τ` carries NO tangent — `Dual::constant(τ)`, §51.9 repair). Because the seed is bound
to the **node value** θ_r (not a continuous sample position), septic-Hermite stencil width is
captured *inside* `b_k^{(r)}` by dual arithmetic and routed to the owning region — there is no
cross-region leakage of the accumulated gradient. The supports are **disjoint** ⇒ the K columns are
structurally distinct ⇒ NOT the degenerate broadcast.

**Cotangent accumulation (NORMATIVE — genuine reverse, O(1) in K).** The backward sweep is exactly
§51.9 with the accumulation generalised to K columns at each step `k = n … 1`:

    grad[r] += ⟨λ_k, b_k^{(r)}⟩,    r = 0 … K-1 ,
    λ_{k-1} = Jᵀ λ_k   (= apply_transpose_step, F^⊤=F for const-per-region a) .

All K columns reuse the SAME replayed `u_{k-1}` and the SAME single cotangent `λ` — one backward
walk yields all K gradients. Forward dual-AD needs `O(K)` trajectory passes (one tangent seed per
region); the reverse sweep is `O(1)`-in-K trajectory passes at `O(√n)` memory. **K=1** is the case
`K=1, Ω_0=Ω`: seed everywhere, one column, identical arithmetic to §51.9 ⇒ byte-identical (regression).

**Scope (NORMATIVE — NARROW).** Self-adjoint **const-per-region** `a` only; region boundaries are
**DoF-aligned**. Variable-a within a region, non-self-adjoint kernels, or non-DoF-aligned regions
are OUT of scope and MUST fail-loud (`SemiflowError::UnsupportedOperation`). This preserves the
§51.5 narrow-linear/self-adjoint boundary.

**Gates / oracle (cite).** `G_REVERSE_AD_GRADIENT` is extended to a **K-vector FD-parity** check:
each `grad[r]` matches a central difference perturbing only `θ_r` to `< 1e-9` relative (§51.6 (i)
generalised to K). `G_REVERSE_AD_ADVANTAGE` (§51.9) now binds genuinely at K>1: with the region
kernel, `ratio(64)/ratio(1) ≥ 8`. New sympy oracle `scripts/verify_reverse_ad_kvector.py` proves
`grad[r] = ∂J/∂θ_r` analytically for a small closed-form K-region setup; prints
`T_REVERSE_AD_KVECTOR PASS` (RELEASE_BLOCKING, runs in `test-fast`).

---

## §52 — Tensor-train Chernoff: escaping the curse via the state carrier (v9.0.0 Shift C RESOLUTION, NORMATIVE)

> **§52 STATUS — v9.0.0 SHIPPED A SEPARABILITY TRIVIALITY; v9.1.0 makes it a GENUINE coupled escape (ADR-0159 Amendment 1).**
> **HONEST CORRECTION (2026-06-10, v9.1.0):** the v9.0.0 `TtChernoff::step` applied ONLY per-axis
> independent shifts (`apply_per_axis_shift`, bond indices are pure spectators), so its evolution
> operator was exactly `⊗ⱼKⱼ` — the TT-rank was frozen at the IC's rank forever and `tt_round` could
> only *remove* rank, never control evolution-induced growth (there was none). This is IDENTICALLY the
> Strang⊗/AxisLift path that shipped in v0.5.0 (§52.3 admits it). The "linear r≈d/2 curse-escape" was
> validated ONLY by `tests/g_gridless_ttrank.rs`, which is pure linear algebra on a hand-picked Gaussian
> precision matrix and **never instantiates `TtChernoff`**. So the v9.0.0 evolver's curse-escape was a
> **separability triviality** — it did nothing a `d`-fold independent 1D solve does not.
>
> **v9.1.0 (this section, NORMATIVE):** a new additive evolver **`CoupledTtChernoff`** applies GENUINE
> cross-axis coupling — pair-bond mixed-derivative operators `τρ_{jk}√(a_ja_k)·(D1_j⊗D1_k)` (the
> correlated Fokker–Planck / multi-asset Black–Scholes cross term) that inflate the bonds between the
> coupled cores (real cross-axis work) — followed by TT-rounding that re-compresses to the intrinsic
> correlated-Gaussian rank. **Feasibility was probed FIRST** (`scripts/tt_coupled_evolver_probe.py`,
> `scripts/tt_coupling_scaling.py`): applying a coupled Chernoff step to a **rank-1 separable IC** grows
> the rank from 1 to a BOUNDED 4–5 (no 4ⁿ blow-up), tracking the analytic semigroup; **local/banded
> coupling → peak rank O(1) independent of d** (genuine curse escape on a NON-separable operator); dense
> correlated-Gaussian coupling → ~⌊d/2⌋ (polynomial). The shipped v9.0.0 evolver provably cannot reach
> this. The rank-1 separable path (no coupling) MUST still collapse bit-identically to Strang⊗ (§52.3,
> now ENFORCED by `G_TT_STRANG_IDENTITY`). Gates: NEW **`g_tt_coupled`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING; runs the
> coupled evolver, asserts rank GREW from a rank-1 IC, rank polynomial, accuracy vs a genuinely-coupled
> closed-form reference) and NEW **`T_TT_COUPLED_RANK`** oracle (proves the per-step rank bound ON THE
> EVOLVER, closing the v9.0.0 "precision-matrix test never runs the evolver" gap). The old
> `G_TT_CHERNOFF_DIMSCALING` is KEPT as the diagonal-A separable rank-1 reduction check; its vacuous
> "poly-in-d on a constant-rank-2 IC" Regime-H verdict is REMOVED (§52.5).
>
> **Honest scope (NORMATIVE):** the curse escape is GENUINE for the **correlated-Gaussian / linear
> cross-diffusion class** (local coupling O(1); dense correlated-Gaussian polynomial ⌊d/2⌋, Rohrbach et
> al.). **General off-diagonal A with a slowly-decaying precision spectrum, variable-coefficient, and
> nonlinear generators remain RESEARCH-TRACK** — there the rank is NOT algebraically capped and no
> representation escapes the curse (§52.4/§52.6). This residual limit is real and disclosed, not hidden.
> **Narrow novelty (unchanged, Grade B, §52.7):** Chernoff-product-formula step-truncation TT integrator
> + `no_std`/deterministic/rank-1-exact envelope. **Cross-reference**: §50 (the refuted
> particle/spatial-merge form — d=2 validated primitive + documented negative result, UNTOUCHED);
> §10/§11 (tensor product, Strang⊗ — the rank-1 special case of §52).

### §52.1 — The carrier principle: why the curse was never in the evolver (NORMATIVE)

The four prior reframes of the gridless high-dimensional problem (§50.7 research record) all kept the
state in a particle representation (P weighted Diracs) and attacked the estimator or the judged axis.
All re-encountered the curse through the spatial-merge reduction: any grid-based particle reducer that
needs `m` bins per axis to hold accuracy requires a working set of `O(m^d)` — the curse of
dimensionality re-entering through the reduction grid, not through the evolver (§50.7 INTRINSIC LIMIT,
ADR-0155 Amendment). The breakthrough (and the deepest refutation of the prior reframes): **the curse
is an artifact of the CARRIER (the explicit particle representation), not of the Chernoff evolver
itself.** The evolver is cheap and separable for all `d`; the carrier between steps is where the
exponential cost lives. The resolution: hold the state as a **low-rank tensor-train (TT)**
$$
u(i_1,\dots,i_d) = G_1[i_1] \cdot G_2[i_2] \cdots G_d[i_d], \qquad G_k \in \mathbb{R}^{r_{k-1}\times n \times r_k}, \tag{52.1}
$$
with storage `O(d·n·r²)` — **linear in `d`**, no exponential, **iff the TT-rank `r` stays bounded**.

### §52.2 — Per-axis Chernoff shift as a rank-preserving operator (NORMATIVE — Grade A)

The per-axis Chernoff shift `x_j ↦ x_j ± h_j` (with `h_j = 2√(a_j τ)`) is a permutation/bidiagonal
matrix along axis `j`, and the ¼,¼,½ weighting is a rank-≤3 banded combination of `{shift⁺, shift⁻, id}`
along that one axis. **Kazeev–Khoromskij (SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 33(3):742–758, 2012)** prove
explicitly that discrete shift / Laplace operators admit exact QTT representations with ranks bounded
by a small constant **independent of the number of dimensions and of the grid resolution** — the
Chernoff step's component operators are exactly these primitives.

A TT-operator acting within a **single mode** (touching core `G_j` only) inflates the adjacent bond
rank by at most the operator's own mode-rank (≤ 2–3) and leaves all other bond ranks unchanged. One
full Chernoff step sweeps `d` single-axis sub-steps; pre-rounding, the bond rank grows by at most a
small constant factor. **This is bounded growth, not blow-up, per step** (standard TT-operator algebra;
Oseledets 2011). After each step, a **deterministic TT-rounding** (truncated SVD per bond, threshold
`ε`) re-compresses to the intrinsic rank of the current state with quasi-optimal error ≤ `√(d−1)·ε` in
Frobenius norm (Oseledets quasi-optimality theorem). The rounding is the only non-trivial kernel; every
other computation is a closed-form shift. This rounding is deterministic and bit-reproducible (one-sided
Jacobi SVD, no LAPACK, ~150 LoC in `tt_core.rs`), preserving the project's determinism headline.

**NORMATIVE (rank-preserving step)**: One complete Chernoff step of `TtChernoff` consists of `d`
sequential single-axis shift-and-weight sub-operations followed by one TT-rounding at tolerance `ε`.
No sub-step may be omitted (each axis must be swept, mirroring the §50.2 d-dim sweep mandate). The
rounding MUST be applied after the full `d`-sub-step pass; rounding after each individual sub-step is
non-conformant (different rank trajectory and different error constant).

#### §52.2 AMENDMENT 1 (v9.1.0-s3, 2026-06-11) — per-axis shift is a fixed-width band, not a single permutation (NORMATIVE)

The per-axis Chernoff shift is realised as a **fixed-width (`w`-band) interpolation shift**
`Sₕ = Σ_{m=0}^{w-1} c_m(h/dx)·P_{s₀+m}`, `s₀ = ⌊h/dx⌋`, with `c_m` the cubic-Lagrange (`w=4`)
interpolation weights of the off-lattice displacement `h = 2√(aτ)`. Each band `P_{s₀+m}` is a
permutation (QTT-op-rank ≤ 2, Kazeev–Khoromskij); the `w`-band sum has QTT-op-rank ≤ `2w` and
TT-rounds to a small constant **independent of grid resolution and of `d`** (measured rank 3 for cubic,
∀ `L∈{6,8,10}`, `d∈{3..6}`; `T_TT_BAND_SHIFT_RANK`). The interpolation weights carry the
continuum-exact displacement, so the kernel converges `O(τ²)` — resolving the §52.9 Amendment 1
integer-shift quantization floor. The lattice constrains the operator *support* (on-grid bands →
rank-O(1)) but NOT the *displacement* (off-grid `h` → convergence); these are separated onto the band
level vs the weight level (TRIZ separation-in-structure, this spec §5.1 of `.dev-docs/specs/v9.1.0-s3-triz-resolution.md`).

- **`T_TT_BAND_SHIFT_RANK`** (NEW, sympy+numeric, `scripts/tt_band_shift_kit.py`, `test-fast`,
  RELEASE_BLOCKING math-fidelity): PROVE (1) the cubic-Lagrange band weights `c_m(t)` sum to 1 and
  reproduce a degree-3 polynomial displacement exactly (interpolation-order proof); (2) each band is a
  permutation (QTT-op-rank ≤2); (3) the `w`-band sum has QTT-op-rank ≤ `2w` and the assembled
  operator's measured rank ≤ a stated constant independent of `L`. Prints `T_TT_BAND_SHIFT_RANK PASS/FAIL`.

### §52.3 — Rank-1 special case = Strang⊗ tensor product (NORMATIVE reduction)

**For diagonal, constant `A` and a product initial condition** (separable `u_0 = ⊗_j u_0^{(j)}`), the
TT-rank of `u_0` is 1 (one core per axis, no bond interaction). The per-axis shift acts on each core
independently; the bonds never inflate; the TT-rounding is never invoked (rank stays 1 exactly). The
resulting evolution is **identically the Strang⊗ tensor product** `e^{τL} = ⊗_j e^{τL_j}` (Theorem 7,
§10.3) computed via `AxisLift`/`Strang2D`/`Strang3D` — the already-shipped path, `O(d·n)`-exact, no
SVD, no curse. This is an algebraic identity, not an approximation: §10.3 Theorem 7 proves separability
of the semigroup under `[L_j, L_k] = 0` (satisfied for diagonal `A`) and the Chernoff product of
separable operators on a product state is a product state. **Consequence (NORMATIVE):** the rank-1 fast
path MUST branch directly to the `AxisLift`/`Strang` path without invoking the TT rounding machinery.
`TtChernoff::new` with a rank-1 `TtState` MUST produce results bit-identical to `Strang2D`/`Strang3D`
at equal `n` and `τ`.

#### §52.3 AMENDMENT 1 (2026-06-10, v9.1.0) — the "bit-identical to Strang2D/Strang3D" clause was FALSE; corrected gate (NORMATIVE, supersedes the last sentence above)

**Honest correction.** The sentence "`TtChernoff::new` with a rank-1 `TtState` MUST produce results
bit-identical to `Strang2D`/`Strang3D`" is **mathematically false as written** and is hereby
superseded. The error conflates two distinct objects:

1. **"Strang⊗"** — the *abstract tensor-product structure* `e^{τL} = ⊗_j e^{τL_j}` (Theorem 7, §10.3).
   The TT rank-1 path IS this structure (each core evolves independently, no bond inflation). This part
   of §52.3 is correct and stands.
2. **`Strang2D`/`Strang3D` — the *concrete shipped types*** (`src/strang2d.rs:90`, `src/strang3d.rs`).
   These are `Strang2D<X, Y, F>` parameterised over *arbitrary* inner `ChernoffFunction`s. In practice
   the inner is `DiffusionChernoff` (`src/diffusion.rs`), whose 1D kernel is a **ζ-A Gauss–Hermite /
   Catmull–Rom node-sampling quadrature** (`apply_at_node_f64`, S-shift + ζ-A τ²-correction,
   `f.sample()` continuous interpolation). `Strang2D` further composes it as a **palindromic
   3-leg sandwich** `X(τ/2) ∘ Y(τ) ∘ X(τ/2)` (`apply_strang2d_into`, `strang2d.rs:309`).

`TtChernoff`'s 1D kernel is a **¼·shift(+s) + ¼·shift(−s) + ½·id three-branch *integer-index periodic*
shift** on the discrete grid (`apply_per_axis_shift`, `tt_chernoff.rs:276`), with NO half-step
splitting (it applies a full step per axis per `step`, `tt_chernoff.rs:220`). These are **two different
discrete operators** that *both consistently approximate the same continuous semigroup* `e^{τL_j}` but
are NOT the same finite map: different stencil (3-branch shift vs Gauss–Hermite sampling), different
boundary (periodic wrap vs Catmull–Rom interpolation), different composition (single full step vs
palindromic half/full/half). Their outputs differ at **O(τ²) discretisation order**, not at ULP level.
Therefore 0-ULP — indeed any fixed-ULP — equality between `TtChernoff` and the real `Strang2D` type is
**provably UNACHIEVABLE**, and the hand-rolled `shift_1d_step` reference previously used in the test was
*neither* the real `Strang2D` *nor* the `TtChernoff` kernel — it silently invented a third operator that
happens to match the TT shift, so the ≤16-ULP it observed measured only FP accumulation order between
two re-implementations of the SAME shift, proving nothing about §52.3.

**This is a genuine contract flaw of the §51.4 class** (the clause asserted an identity that the code
cannot satisfy), NOT an engineer over-relaxation of an achievable gate. See the ruling table below.

**Corrected NORMATIVE gate — `G_TT_STRANG_IDENTITY` (3 sub-gates, RELEASE_BLOCKING):**

- **Gate A — separable-structure 0-ULP identity (THE §52.3 identity, ENFORCED at 0 ULP).**
  The mathematically true and ULP-exact statement of §52.3 is *internal to the TT machinery*: for a
  rank-1 `TtState` and diagonal `A` (no coupling), the TT evolution is **identical to applying the
  per-axis TT shift kernel `K_j` independently on each core, with NO bond inflation and NO SVD
  invoked**. The gate MUST verify, **byte-for-byte (`to_bits()` equality, 0 ULP)**:
  (i) after `evolve`, `state.peak_rank() == 1` (no bond inflation — `tt_round` never raised rank);
  (ii) each evolved core's data equals the standalone per-axis result `K_j^{N_steps}` applied to the
       IC slice `u_0^{(j)}`, **up to the documented `tt_round` norm-redistribution convention**: a
       rank-1 chain `G_0 · G_1 · … · G_{d−1}` is invariant under `(G_k, G_{k+1}) ↦ (G_k/λ, λ·G_{k+1})`,
       so the gate compares the **scale-invariant reconstructed tensor entries** (or the
       `inner_separable` functional, which is identically scale-invariant) — NOT the raw per-core bytes.
       Against the *TT shift kernel itself* (the same `K_j` the evolver uses, applied standalone), this
       reconstruction IS **0 ULP** (identical arithmetic, identical fold order). This is the
       separable-path-vs-separable-path identity; it is kept at 0 ULP and is the honest enforcement of
       §52.3's true content.

- **Gate B — consistency-vs-real-`Strang2D`/`Strang3D` (the cross-operator check, JUSTIFIED tolerance).**
  Because the real `Strang2D<DiffusionChernoff,…>` and `TtChernoff` are *different O(τ²) discretisations*
  of the *same* `e^{TL}`, the gate MUST instantiate the **REAL shipped `Strang2D`/`Strang3D` type**
  (`Strang2D::new(DiffusionChernoff_x, DiffusionChernoff_y)`, NOT a hand-rolled reference) on the same
  IC, `n`, `τ`, and assert the two evolved states **agree to discretisation order**, not to ULP:
  `‖u_TT − u_Strang2D‖_∞ / ‖u_Strang2D‖_∞ ≤ C_consist`, with `C_consist = 5·10⁻²` at `N = 32`,
  `T = 0.3` (both schemes are O(τ²)-consistent; the bound is the sum of their truncation errors, NOT
  a fudge — it is loose because it bounds a real modelling difference, and is tightened as O(τ²) under
  step refinement, which the gate MAY additionally check via a 2-point slope ≥ 1.8). This closes the
  audit finding ("TT rank-1 IS the shipped Strang⊗") *honestly*: the test now TOUCHES the real
  `Strang2D` and proves the TT rank-1 path reproduces the shipped separable solver **to the accuracy
  both claim**, while not pretending a false bit-identity.

- **Gate C — `CoupledTtChernoff(None) ≡ TtChernoff` 0-ULP (same code path, ENFORCED at 0 ULP).**
  `CoupledTtChernoff` with `CouplingTopology::None` MUST be **byte-for-byte identical** (`to_bits()` on
  every core datum) to `TtChernoff` on the same rank-1 IC — both take the identical diagonal-sweep code
  path (no coupling operator fires). This is a true 0-ULP gate (no rounding-convention escape) and is
  the additive-compatibility invariant of §52.9. It stays at 0 ULP, unchanged.

**Reference rule (NORMATIVE):** the hand-rolled `shift_1d_step` / `reference_1d_evolved` helper is
**FORBIDDEN** as a §52.3 reference. Gate A's reference is the actual `TtChernoff` per-axis kernel
applied standalone (or the scale-invariant reconstruction of the evolved TT). Gate B's reference is the
**actual shipped `Strang2D`/`Strang3D` type**. Gate C's reference is `TtChernoff` itself.

### §52.4 — Gaussian rank cap: the curse-escape condition (NORMATIVE — Grade A)

**Rohrbach, Dolgov, Grasedyck, Scheichl**, *Rank Bounds for Approximating Gaussian Densities in the
Tensor-Train Format* (SIAM/ASA J. Uncertainty Quantification 10(3):1191–1224, 2022; arXiv:2001.08187)
establish the decisive result: for a Gaussian density `N(μ, Σ)`, the TT-rank is governed by the
**singular spectrum of the subdiagonal blocks of the precision matrix** `Σ⁻¹`. Specifically, the
off-diagonal block of `Σ⁻¹` for the split `{1,…,k} | {k+1,…,d}` has numerical rank at most
`min(k, d−k)` for the Gaussian class, algebraically. Therefore:

$$
r_k \;\leq\; \min(k,\, d - k), \qquad k = 1, \dots, d-1, \tag{52.2}
$$
$$
\text{peak rank} \;\leq\; \lfloor d/2 \rfloor. \tag{52.3}
$$

The peak rank is **capped at `d/2` — linear in `d`, not exponential**. Storage is `O(d·n·(d/2)²) = O(d³·n)` — polynomial in `d`, exponential curse **escaped**. This bound is algebraic (not a heuristic), holds for any precision matrix in the Gaussian class, and is confirmed by the `g_gridless_ttrank` prototype gate (Regime H: dense Cauchy-correlated IC, rank measured ≤ d/2 across d ∈ {4,6,8,10}).

**Cost-wording temper (NORMATIVE, 2026-06-10 — measured Phase-6 behaviour).** The escape is from **exponential `n^d` to POLYNOMIAL in `d`**, not to `O(1)`. Two facts must not be conflated: (a) the dense correlated-Gaussian **peak rank** scales as `⌊d/2⌋` (linear in `d`, slope ≈ 0.79 in the probe — NOT `O(1)`); local/banded coupling has `O(1)` *rank* but still `O(d)` cores. (b) the per-axis mode dimension `n` is a *separate* factor: each core is `r_{k−1}×n×r_k`, so even at fixed rank the storage carries an explicit `n`. The honest cost statement is therefore **`O(d·n·r²)` with `r ≤ ⌊d/2⌋` dense / `r = O(1)` local — i.e. polynomial in both `d` and `n`, never `O(1)`**. Any prior "O(1) cost" phrasing (local topology) refers to `O(1)` *rank per bond*, and must be read as `O(d·n)` *total* storage. The curse-escape claim is "polynomial-in-`d`", full stop.

For the diagonal-A Gaussian case (§52.3), the precision is diagonal: all off-diagonal blocks have rank 0 (zero) → TT-rank = 1 exactly. The §52.3 Strang⊗ reduction is the limit case of the §52.4 Gaussian cap.

**Honest scope boundary (NORMATIVE):** the rank cap (52.2)–(52.3) is proven for the Gaussian class
only. For off-diagonal (non-separable) `A`, variable-coefficient, or nonlinear generators, the
precision matrix is dense and its subdiagonal blocks may have many slowly-decaying singular values; rank
is not algebraically capped. Such operators are **research-track** for `TtChernoff` and are explicitly
out of scope for the `G_TT_CHERNOFF_DIMSCALING` gate.

### §52.5 — Acceptance gate: G_TT_CHERNOFF_DIMSCALING (NORMATIVE — PRE-REGISTERED)

- **`G_TT_CHERNOFF_DIMSCALING`** (`slow-tests`, `--ignored`; file `tests/g_tt_chernoff.rs`): end-to-end
  curse-escape validation for `TtChernoff` on linear diagonal-A (Gaussian) diffusion
  `∂_t u = Σ_j a_j ∂²_{x_j} u` with `a_j = 0.5 + 0.1j`, `T = 1`, `n = 32` nodes/axis,
  `d ∈ {4, 6, 8, 10}`, TT-rounding tolerance `ε = 1e-8`. **Two correlation regimes** (same code,
  different initial condition):

  - **Regime L** (rank-1 separable IC — product of Gaussians): TT-rank constant, r = 1,
    storage `O(d·n)` — optimal polynomial curse-escape. This is the DIAGONAL-A separable reduction
    check; it confirms the rank-1 fast path collapses to Strang⊗ (§52.3).

  **PASS iff ALL of (Regime L only):**
  1. Functional accuracy `|⟨f, u_T⟩_TT − truth| < 5e-3` at each d (truth = closed-form Gaussian `Σ_T = Σ_0 + 2T·A`).
  2. Peak TT-rank stays r = 1 (separable diagonal-A — any r > 1 is a structural bug). **HARD ASSERT.**
  3. TT storage sub-exponential vs naive `n^d` at every d where `n^d` is computable.
  4. **Byte-reproducibility**: two independent runs produce bit-identical TT cores.

  **REMOVED (v9.1.0 — was vacuous, ADR-0159 Amendment 1):** the v9.0.0 "Regime H" sub-gate asserted a
  log-rank slope `< 0.70` on a **constant-rank-2 hand-built IC** whose reference was computed as two
  INDEPENDENT 1D evolutions — a separable superposition that stays rank-2 under the separable v9.0.0
  evolver, proving NOTHING about cross-axis coupling. Its "POLYNOMIAL-ESCAPE-H ✓" verdict on a flat
  rank-2 IC is deleted. **The genuine high-dimensional curse-escape claim is now validated by
  `g_tt_coupled` (§52.9), which runs the COUPLED evolver on a rank-1 IC and asserts the rank GREW** —
  the anti-separability-triviality check the v9.0.0 gate lacked. The `g_gridless_ttrank` analytic
  rank-prototype is retained as a *theory* check (validates the Rohrbach Gaussian cap on the precision
  matrix) but is explicitly LABELLED as not exercising the evolver (§52.9).

- **Sign convention**: the rank-slope gate is `< 0.70` (smaller = better; smaller slope = more bounded
  rank growth), the opposite direction from the order-of-accuracy gates (`≥` threshold, larger order is
  better) — stated explicitly to avoid the sign trap documented in §50.6.

### §52.6 — Relation to §50: what §52 resolves and what it does not (NORMATIVE)

§50 documents the particle / spatial-merge GridlessChernoff: a **correct but narrow** d=2-validated
deterministic d-dim primitive whose high-d thesis was refuted on two independent axes — (1) the
spatial-merge reduction re-introduces the curse (INTRINSIC LIMIT, §50.7), and (2) the variance claim
was not confirmed at ≥2× (G_GRIDLESS_VARIANCE NO-GO). The particle form ships retained as the d=2
primitive and as the documented negative result.

§52 resolves the curse for the **diagonal-A Gaussian class** by replacing the particle carrier with a
TT carrier. It does NOT retroactively change the §50 negative result, which stands for the particle
representation across all four reframes. §50 and §52 are complementary: §50 is the honest record of
what was tried and refuted under the particle representation; §52 is the escape that works because it
changes the representation entirely. For operators outside the diagonal-A Gaussian class (dense
correlation, variable coefficient, nonlinear) §52's rank is not capped — the curse is intrinsic to the
solution's rank structure, and no representation — particle, grid, or tensor-train — escapes it (§52.4,
Rohrbach–Dolgov–Grasedyck–Scheichl).

### §52.7 — Narrow novelty statement (NORMATIVE — Grade B)

**Step-truncation TT integrators** (explicit time step followed by TT-rounding) are an established
method class: Rodgers–Venturi (*Step-Truncation Methods for Nonlinear Evolution Equations on Tensor
Manifolds*; arXiv:2008.00155) define, analyze, and implement this paradigm. **The present construction
is NOT claimed as a novel method class.** The defensible, narrow novelty is:

1. **The explicit step is the Chernoff/Theorem-6 product formula** — closed-form per-axis shifts
   `2√(a_jτ)` with no stencil, no matrix exponential, no Krylov solve (R2 solver-free in the
   strongest sense: arithmetic only, no matrix-vector product). Most step-truncation work uses
   finite-difference or spectral RHS operators; using the Chernoff semigroup approximation as the
   explicit step is, to the literature surveyed, unclaimed.
2. **`no_std` / no-LAPACK / ≤3-dep / bit-reproducible target** — no TT-PDE work surveyed targets this
   engineering envelope. The determinism and embeddability are the same distinctive axis as the broader
   library.
3. **Exact rank-1 collapse to the shipped Strang⊗** (§52.3) — a single code path from `O(d)`-exact
   separable evolution up to rank-r correlated evolution, with no artificial boundary between the two.

Grade **B** (known method class, genuinely unclaimed instantiation + unique engineering envelope).
Do not claim "first solver-free TT semigroup stepper."

### §52.9 — `CoupledTtChernoff`: GENUINE cross-axis coupling (v9.1.0 NORMATIVE — ADR-0159 Amendment 1)

**Why a new evolver.** The v9.0.0 `TtChernoff` applies only mode-local per-axis shifts (bond indices spectators), so it is exactly `⊗ⱼKⱼ` and freezes TT-rank at the IC's rank — a separability triviality (STATUS admonition). To do work a `d`-fold independent 1D solve does NOT, the evolver must introduce genuine cross-axis correlation. `CoupledTtChernoff` is the additive sibling that does so.

**The coupling operator (NORMATIVE).** For a coupled pair `(j,k)` with correlation `ρ_{jk}`, the generator carries a mixed second-derivative cross term `ρ_{jk}√(a_ja_k)·∂_{x_j}∂_{x_k}`. Its discrete operator factorises as `D1_j ⊗ D1_k` (a product of two single-axis first-difference operators) — a **rank-1 TT-operator on the two affected modes** (the ¼/¼/½ Chernoff weighting raises its mode-rank to ≤ 2). Applying it contracts into cores `j…k` and **inflates the bonds in `[j,k)` by ≤ 2** — this is the genuine cross-axis work the v9.0.0 evolver lacked.

**One coupled step (NORMATIVE — v9.1.0-s3 ROUND-4 REPLACEMENT, supersedes the prior round-1/2/3 explicit-additive cross; see §52.9 Amendment 1 STATUS below).**
(1) diagonal per-axis band-split shift sweep (§52.2 Amendment 1 — the separable part, cubic-Lagrange
`w=4`);
(2) **pair sweep (NORMATIVE preferred: spectral / R3, solver-free):** for each coupled pair `(j,k,ρ)`
apply the **exact pair factor** `K_pair = exp(τ_eff·L_pair)`, `L_pair = c_j·∂_j² + c_k·∂_k² + 2r·∂_j∂_k`
(`r=ρ√(a_j a_k)`, `c_j=a_j/#pairs(j)`), realised by the **spectral (FFT-diagonal) apply** over the
`(j,k)` TT slab:

**Boundary-condition scope (NORMATIVE):** the spectral pair factor and the per-axis band-split shift both use a **periodic DFT** (wavenumbers `k = 2πm/n`, wrap `% n`) and are therefore scoped to **PERIODIC boundary conditions on each axis**. Non-periodic (Dirichlet/Neumann/mixed) boundaries are NOT covered by this scheme and remain research-track.

```
K_pair·u = ifft2( exp(τ_eff·symbol) ⊙ fft2(u) ),
symbol(k_j,k_k) = c_j·σ_{D2}(k_j) + c_k·σ_{D2}(k_k) + 2r·σ_{D1}(k_j)·σ_{D1}(k_k),
σ_{D2}(k) = (2cos(k·dx)−2)/dx²,   σ_{D1}(k) = i·sin(k·dx)/dx.
```

The diagonal `exp(τ_eff·symbol)` is built **once per `(pair, τ)`** before the step loop (τ constant
within `evolve`) and reused every step. **No linear solver** (FFT is a fixed unitary + elementwise
scalar `exp` — Theorem-6 R2 honoured throughout, coupling factor included). **The spectral R3 path is
the shipped production implementation** (`crates/semiflow-core/src/tt_spectral.rs` +
`tt_coupled_pair.rs`); the `no_lu_in_coupling` source-scan test confirms no `lu_solve_inplace` or
`dense_expm` outside `#[cfg(test)]`. Fallback: **(R0) dense `expm(τ_eff·L_pair)` via Padé+LU** is
exact and poly-`d` but carries an LU triangular solve per pair (R2 NOT honoured for that factor);
survives as a `#[cfg(test)]` reference only.
For **shared-axis (tridiagonal) topologies** the per-pair factors are Strang-composed (½ forward chain,
½ reverse). `CouplingTopology::None` → no pairs → **bit-identical to `TtChernoff`** (Gate C invariant);
(3) reaction `(1+τc)`;
(4) **ONE TT-rounding** at `ε` (§52.2 convention).

**Exact class (NORMATIVE — v9.1.0).** The supported and EXACT class is: **constant diagonal diffusion
`aⱼ` (drift `b = 0`), scalar reaction `c`, constant correlation `ρ`, TRIDIAGONAL or BLOCK-DISJOINT
ADJACENT pairs only**. Drift (`b ≠ 0`) and non-adjacent pairs are NOT part of the exact class and are
explicitly REJECTED at construction (see fail-loud guards below).

**Fail-loud construction guards (NORMATIVE, v9.1.0).** `CoupledTtChernoff::new` REJECTS at
construction time — hard panic, no silent skip:

(a) **Drift `b ≠ 0`:** any axis `j` with a non-zero drift coefficient `b_j` is rejected with:
    "CoupledTtChernoff drift b≠0 is not supported in v9.1.0 (drift advection unimplemented — ADR-0162
    / §52.9 v9.2.0 deferral); pass b = 0". The per-axis shift is symmetric (mean-preserving); correct
    advective drift requires a directional asymmetric shift not yet built. Pass `b = 0` to `new`.

(b) **Non-adjacent pair `(j,k)` with `k > j+1`:** any non-adjacent pair is rejected with:
    "CoupledTtChernoff non-adjacent pair (j,k) with k>j+1 is not supported in v9.1.0 (only tridiagonal
    / block-disjoint adjacent pairs; true dense coupling deferred to v9.2.0)". Only adjacent pairs
    (tridiagonal / block-disjoint) are supported; non-adjacent pairs would freeze intermediate bonds
    without coupling them.

**Deferred to v9.2.0:**
- **Drift advection (`b ≠ 0`)** — pre-existing limitation surfaced by v9.1.0 QA coverage testing;
  rejected fail-loud rather than silently wrong.
- **True dense / non-adjacent-pair coupling** — non-adjacent pairs `(j,k)` with `k > j+1`; true
  all-pairs dense coupling requires a different contraction schedule.

For the **constant-coefficient correlated-Gaussian class** (with `b = 0` and adjacent pairs) the circulant pair generators pairwise commute
(`probe_commute`, `‖[L₀₁,L₁₂]‖_F ≈ 0`), so the product split is **EXACT** (zero Strang remainder) and
the pair factor is machine-accurate (`d=2 in-Rust self-check rel-L2 = 5.27e-14` spectral evolver
vs dense-expm; `G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT` exactness gate ≤1e-12 vs independent dense `expm(τL_h^{dx})`,
`d∈{3,4}`, `ρ≠0` — RELEASE_BLOCKING, **PASSES**). For variable-coef/nonlinear
coefficients (research-track, §52.4), the product split is `O(τ²)` Strang and rank is not algebraically
capped. Pair-factor TT-op-rank = `O(1)` (measured 6, constant in `n,d`; `probe_pair_rank`,
`probe_adjudicate_spectral_cost`), so the §52.4 curse-escape holds. **The round-2 "rotation + band-shift
on rotated axes / no solver" description was a design error — a shift along a rotated eigendirection is
inherently two-axis (op-rank 6 ≠ 1; s3 §11.2 of `.dev-docs/specs/v9.1.0-s3-triz-resolution.md`) and
cannot be a pure per-axis shift; the solver-free property is recovered by the spectral basis (R3), NOT
a real-space band-shift.**

**Per-step rank bound (NORMATIVE).** Pair-factor TT-op-rank = `O(1)` (measured 6 constant in `n,d`);
post-round peak rank ≤ intrinsic correlated-Gaussian rank: **O(1) rank-per-bond** for local/banded
topology, **⌊d/2⌋** for dense (§52.4, Rohrbach et al.); storage `O(d·n·r²)` polynomial in `d` and `n`,
NOT `O(1)` (see §52.4 cost-wording temper).

- **`T_TT_COUPLED_RANK`** (NORMATIVE numeric+sympy oracle, `scripts/tt_coupled_kit.py`, RELEASE_BLOCKING
  math-fidelity, `test-fast`): PROVE pair-operator mode-rank ≤ 2 and post-round rank = analytic
  correlated-Gaussian precision-block rank (⌊d/2⌋ dense, O(1) tridiagonal). Prints `T_TT_COUPLED_RANK PASS/FAIL`.

- **`G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT`** (EXACTNESS gate, RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`; `#[ignore]`-gated for
  ~140s runtime only — spectral R3 is shipped and the gate **PASSES**):
  `‖CoupledTtChernoff(T) − expm(τ·L_h^{dx})‖_rel ≤ 1e-12` (Frobenius, vs the independent dense
  same-grid matrix-exponential reference), `d∈{3,4}`, `ρ=0.6≠0`, `τ∼0.35dx²` (non-integer `h/dx`,
  per-level values reported by the gate: d=4 n=5 → h/dx≈0.92; d=3 → h/dx≈1.07; anti-vacuity), HARD assert. In-Rust results: d=3 (ρ=0.6, n∈{9,11,13}: 1.6e-13–4.5e-13),
  d=4 (ρ=0.4, n∈{5,7}: 5.2e-14, 1.2e-13). No slope gate (degenerate at machine floor for the exact
  scheme; the only truncation-bearing regime is variable-coef, out of v9.1.0 scope). The
  `no_lu_in_coupling` source-scan test confirms no `lu_solve_inplace`/`dense_expm` outside
  `#[cfg(test)]` on the production coupling path.

- **`g_tt_coupled`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `slow-tests`, `--ignored`, `tests/g_tt_coupled.rs`): run
  `CoupledTtChernoff` on `d∈{4,6,8,10}` from a rank-1 separable IC. **PASS iff ALL (HARD ASSERTS):**
  1. **Coupling actually happened** — evolved-state peak rank `> 1` (anti-triviality).
  2. **Rank polynomial** — log-rank slope `< 0.70` ON THE EVOLVER OUTPUT (tridiagonal ≈ 0; dense ≈ ⌊d/2⌋).
  3. **Exactness gate passes** — `G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT` ≤1e-12 (spectral R3 is shipped; gate PASSES;
     `#[ignore]`+`slow-tests` for runtime only).
  4. **Cost sub-exponential** vs naive `n^d` where computable.
  5. **Byte-reproducible** (two runs bit-identical cores).

- **`G_TT_STRANG_IDENTITY`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, `tests/g_tt_strang_identity.rs`): **Gate A:** rank-1
  separable-path 0-ULP identity. **Gate B:** consistency `≤5e-2` vs real shipped `Strang2D`/`Strang3D`.
  **Gate C:** `CoupledTtChernoff(None)` 0-ULP vs `TtChernoff`. Hand-rolled `shift_1d_step` FORBIDDEN.

#### §52.9 AMENDMENT 1 — STATUS: RESOLVED (v9.1.0-s3-triz, 2026-06-11; ADR-0162)

**Prior STATUS:** BOUNDARY (fundamental) — recorded 2026-06-10 under the integer-shift Chernoff scheme.

**VERDICT: RESOLVED.** The prior boundary rested on the premise that "a fractional shift destroys the
QTT-rank guarantee" — **measured FALSE** (s3 §6.1: cubic-band shift rank 3, constant in `L`,`d`;
convergence 7.7e-5 → 1.2e-6 where integer plateaus at 0.20). The integer-shift O(1) quantization floor
is removed by a fixed-width band-split interpolation shift (§52.2 Amendment 1) whose bands stay
permutations (rank-O(1)) while the band-weights realise the exact displacement (convergence). The cross
floor (round 2) is removed by the spectral (FFT-diagonal) pair factor (round 4), which is **exact** for
the constant-coef correlated-Gaussian class and **no-solver** (Theorem-6 R2 honoured). The `G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT` exactness gate (≤1e-12 vs independent dense `expm(τL_h^{dx})`, `d∈{3,4}`,
`ρ≠0`) is **REINSTATED** (formerly withdrawn under the BOUNDARY verdict) and is the binding arbiter.
The spectral R3 factor is **SHIPPED** (`crates/semiflow-core/src/tt_spectral.rs` + `tt_coupled_pair.rs`)
and the gate **PASSES** (`#[ignore]`+`slow-tests` for ~140s runtime; RELEASE_BLOCKING, green). The
"exact / no-solver / third S-curve" language is therefore **CERTIFIED** for this session.

**Historical record preserved (true about the integer-shift scheme):** The four points of the prior
Amendment 1 (cross-term scaling bug real-but-not-causal; τ-only-at-fixed-`dx` diverges; joint-parabolic
still plateaus at O(1) for the integer-shift; integer-shift error tracked by rounding residual) remain
TRUE about the integer-shift carrier and are archived in `.dev-docs/specs/v9.1.0-s3-triz-resolution.md`
§8–§10.

**Gates that apply (NORMATIVE):**
- `T_TT_BAND_SHIFT_RANK` (P1, §52.2 Amendment 1) — RELEASE_BLOCKING
- `G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT` / `g_tt_coupled_converge` (P4', exactness ≤1e-12, RELEASE_BLOCKING) — **PASSES** (spectral R3 shipped; `#[ignore]`+`slow-tests` for runtime only)
- `g_tt_coupled` (P5, rank/poly-d, `d∈{4,6,8,10}`) — RELEASE_BLOCKING
- `G_TT_STRANG_IDENTITY` (Gate A/B/C) — RELEASE_BLOCKING

**Independent-control rule (NORMATIVE, reaffirmed):** the `G_TT_COUPLED_EXACT` reference MUST be
`expm(τ·L_h^{dx})` (stable/exact, dense same-grid) — NEVER the coupled TT operator's own re-implementation and NEVER the τ-only-at-fixed-`dx` sub-check (mis-specified for any shift-Chernoff scheme, drives `h/dx→0` into divergence — s3 §10.3).

- **`G_TT_STRANG_IDENTITY`** (RELEASE_BLOCKING, NEW, `tests/g_tt_strang_identity.rs`): the §52.3 NORMATIVE requirement, now ENFORCED via the **corrected three-sub-gate spec of §52.3 AMENDMENT 1** (the original "0 ULP vs `Strang2D`/`Strang3D`" wording was a contract flaw — those concrete types use a different O(τ²) discretisation than `TtChernoff`'s 3-branch shift, so cross-operator bit-identity is unachievable). **Gate A:** separable-path 0-ULP identity — rank stays 1 (no bond inflation, no SVD) and the scale-invariant TT reconstruction / `inner_separable` functional is **0 ULP** vs the standalone `TtChernoff` per-axis kernel. **Gate B:** consistency vs the **REAL shipped `Strang2D`/`Strang3D` type** (NOT a hand-rolled reference) to **justified discretisation tolerance** `‖u_TT − u_Strang2D‖_∞/‖u_Strang2D‖_∞ ≤ 5e-2` at `N=32, T=0.3` (both O(τ²); bounds the real modelling difference). **Gate C:** `CoupledTtChernoff(None)` byte-identical (0 ULP) to `TtChernoff`. The hand-rolled `shift_1d_step` reference is FORBIDDEN. Closes the audit finding that the §52.3 clause had no test that touches the real `Strang2D`.

### §52.8 — References

- I. Oseledets, *Tensor-Train Decomposition*, **SIAM J. Sci. Comput.** 33(5):2295–2317 (2011) — TT
  storage `O(d·n·r²)`; quasi-optimal TT-rounding error ≤ `√(d−1)·ε`. **A.**
- V. Kazeev, B. Khoromskij, *Low-Rank Explicit QTT Representation of the Laplace Operator and Its
  Inverse*, **SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl.** 33(3):742–758 (2012) — explicit, exact QTT-Laplace with
  ranks independent of dimension and grid size; shift/permutation matrices low QTT-rank. (Q1 anchor,
  Grade A operator side.) **A.**
- P. Rohrbach, S. Dolgov, L. Grasedyck, R. Scheichl, *Rank Bounds for Approximating Gaussian
  Densities in the Tensor-Train Format*, **SIAM/ASA J. Uncertainty Quantification** 10(3):1191–1224
  (2022); arXiv:2001.08187 — TT-rank of a Gaussian density governed by the singular spectrum of the
  precision-matrix subdiagonal blocks; rank ≤ d/2 for the Gaussian class (eq. 52.2–52.3). (The
  decisive Q2 paper for the curse-escape condition.) **A.**
- S. Dolgov, B. Khoromskij, I. Oseledets, *Fast Solution of Parabolic Problems in the TT/QTT Format
  with Initial Application to the Fokker–Planck Equation*, **SIAM J. Sci. Comput.** 34(6):A3016–A3038
  (2012) — parabolic/Fokker–Planck solvable in TT/QTT when the solution is low-rank. **A.**
- D. Rodgers, D. Venturi, *Step-Truncation Methods for Nonlinear Evolution Equations on Tensor
  Manifolds* (arXiv:2008.00155) — **prior-art cap**: explicit step + TT-rounding is the proposed
  paradigm's method class; rank-adaptive, convergence proven. **A.**
- *Full grid solution for multi-asset options pricing with tensor networks*, arXiv:2601.00009 (2026) —
  QTT ranks polynomial-in-d, polylog-in-grid; correlated basket/max-min at d=3–15. **A.**
- **Internal**: math §10.3 / §10.7-bis / §10.8 (Theorem 7, separable `e^{tL} = ⊗_j e^{tL_j}` EXACT;
  `AxisLift`/`Strang2D`/`Strang3D` — the rank-1 fast path of §52.3); §50 / ADR-0155 (particle
  GridlessChernoff — the refuted form whose §50.7 INTRINSIC LIMIT is the motivation for the carrier
  change); ADR-0159 (Shift C RESOLUTION decision); ADR-0154 (v9.0.0 umbrella, third S-curve).

## §53 — S³ honest-scope public API: boundary-as-type wrappers (v9.2.0, ADR-0169)

This section serves as the umbrella cross-reference for the five S³ POC evolvers
promoted to a curated public surface in v9.2.0.  Each sub-section below points to
the existing mathematical treatment and records the RELEASE-BLOCKING gate that
constitutes the proof obligation.

The ADR-0169 design decision: three honesty layers — type wall, feature gate,
rustdoc stanza.  No new mathematics is introduced here; §53 is a navigation aid
only.

### §53.1 — `S3DriftSpectralEvolver` (constant-coefficient drift+diffusion)

Mathematical basis: §52.1 (Fourier symbol, per-axis complex exponential), ADR-0164.

**Class boundary (type wall)**: `a: Vec<F>` constructor argument encodes only
per-axis constants; variable `a(x)` is structurally unrepresentable.

**RELEASE-BLOCKING gate**: `g_s3_drift_spectral` — exactness ≤ 1e-12 vs independent
dense Padé `expm`; rank-preservation under drift; cost-scaling at `d ∈ {8,10}`.

### §53.2 — `S3DenseCouplingEvolver` (rank-1-dense all-pairs coupling)

Mathematical basis: ADR-0165 (dense spectral symbol via `dense_expsym_nd`/`dense_coupling_evolve`; rank-1-dense `D = diag(a) + λ·g·gᵀ` Fourier diagonalisation).

**Class boundary (type wall)**: only `rank1_dense` constructor exists; generic
full-rank `D` is an info-theoretic wall (no public raw-`D` constructor).

**RELEASE-BLOCKING gate**: `g_s3_dense_coupling` — non-vacuous rank-2-contrast
proves generic full-rank coupling is NOT curse-escaped.

### §53.3 — `S3VarCoefEvolver` (additive-separable variable coefficient)

Mathematical basis: §52 operator splitting with variable `aⱼ(xⱼ)` per axis,
ADR-0166.

**Class boundary (type wall)**: `AxisCoef<F>` stores per-axis 1-D arrays; a
truly non-separable `a(x,y)` is UNREPRESENTABLE by the type.

**RELEASE-BLOCKING gate**: `g_s3_varcoef_spectral` — convergence slope ≤ −1.9
on `cos(x)sin(y)·∂²ₓ` (the floor case); wrong-operator test fails loud.

### §53.4 — `S3NonSepVarCoefEvolver` (low-CP-rank non-separable variable coefficient)

Mathematical basis: CP decomposition of `a(x)`, Strang splitting per ADR-0167.

**Class boundary (type wall)**: `CpCoef<F>` holds a fixed-`m` Vec of `CpTerm`;
generic full-CP-rank `a(x)` (exponentially many terms) is UNREPRESENTABLE.
Parabolicity `c(x) > 0` is checked fail-loud at construction.

**RELEASE-BLOCKING gate**: `g_s3_nonsep_varcoef` — slope ≤ −1.9 on
`cos(x)sin(y)·∂²ₓ` (the §53.3 floor case).

### §53.5 — `S3BurgersColeHopf` and `S3ReactionDiffusion` (nonlinear)

Mathematical basis: §53 ADR-0168 (Cole-Hopf exact transform, Strang-split RD).

**Class boundaries (type wall)**:
- `S3BurgersColeHopf`: only `nu > 0` constructible (parabolicity wall).
- `S3ReactionDiffusion`: reaction limited to closed-form-flow `Reaction` enum;
  generic/transcendental `f` is UNREPRESENTABLE.  Logistic IC must be in `(0,1)`
  (fail-loud, promoted from `debug_assert`).

**RELEASE-BLOCKING gate**: `g_s3_nonlinear` — Cole-Hopf sub-gate error ≤ 1e-9;
Strang sub-gate slope ≤ −1.9.
